---  
title: Philosophy Language - A Reference Card and Tutorial  
categories: Notes  
subclass: Methodology  
---  
  
## How to Use Layered Terms  
  
Some philosophical terms have more than one valid use. This reference card distinguishes three levels:  
  
**Strict source use (严格原典用法):** how the term works in its primary author, text, or historical setting.  
**Reception use (接受史用法):** how later traditions translate, narrow, expand, or reorganize the term.  
**Contemporary transferable use (当代理论泛用法):** how the term is used across current theory, criticism, social analysis, or interdisciplinary writing.  
  
The rule is simple: do not transfer a term without asking what problem it originally solved, what later traditions changed, and what new problem the term is now being used to solve.  
(基本规则是：不要直接转用一个术语；应先追问它原先解决什么问题，后来传统改变了什么，现在又被用来解决什么新问题。)  
  
## Part 1. Greek Beginnings: Being, Logos, Truth  
  
This chapter treats early Greek philosophical language as a **toolkit for making things thinkable**. It is not a neutral list of “ancient terms.” It is a system for handling several basic problems: change, order, knowledge, appearance, truth, action, and the good life. The original terms matter because philosophical concepts often carry older semantic tensions that disappear in smooth translation. Greek, Latin, German, and French terms should not be replaced too quickly by simple glosses, because their original forms often preserve conceptual resonances needed for reading and writing philosophy.  
  
### 1. The Problem-Situation: Why Greek Philosophy Needed Technical Language  
  
Greek philosophy begins when ordinary speech becomes insufficient for theoretical inquiry. Mythic speech can narrate how the world came to be. Political speech can persuade a public assembly. Poetic speech can display memory, honor, and divine order. But philosophical speech asks a different kind of question: **what must be the case for anything to be intelligible at all?** (哲学言说追问：为了让任何事物成为可理解之物，必须已经具备什么条件？)  
  
The first philosophical problem is therefore not merely “What exists?” It is more precise: **how can something be spoken of as one thing when it appears in many changing forms?** (当事物以多种变化形式出现时，它如何仍能被说成“同一个东西”？)  
  
This problem generates a cluster of concepts: **Being / What-is (存在/所是者; el: τὸ εἶναι / τὸ ὄν)**, **Nature (自然; el: φύσις; la: natura)**, **Origin/Principle (本原/原则; el: ἀρχή; la: principium)**, **Form (形式/相; el: εἶδος; la: forma)**, and **Substance (实体; el: οὐσία; la: substantia)**. These terms are not synonyms. Each solves a different pressure in thought.  
  
**Being / What-is (存在/所是者; el: τὸ εἶναι / τὸ ὄν)** asks: what does it mean for something to be rather than not be?  
**Nature (自然; el: φύσις; la: natura)** asks: what makes a thing grow, emerge, or act according to its own inner tendency?  
**Origin/Principle (本原/原则; el: ἀρχή; la: principium)** asks: from what does something begin, and by what is it governed?  
**Form (形式/相; el: εἶδος; la: forma)** asks: what makes this thing the kind of thing it is?  
**Substance (实体; el: οὐσία; la: substantia)** asks: what persists as the bearer of properties, changes, and predicates?  
  
The tool-use is direct. When reading a Greek-derived philosophical claim, ask: is the author solving a problem of **existence**, **generation**, **principle**, **identity**, or **persistence**? (阅读时应判断：作者正在处理存在、生成、原则、同一性，还是持续性的难题？)  
  
### 2. Being: The Problem of Stability under Change  
  
`Being / What-is (存在/所是者; el: τὸ εἶναι / τὸ ὄν)`  
**Definition:** being as such, or that which is. (存在本身，或一切“是”者的存在性。)  
**Problem solved:** it gives thought a way to ask what remains thinkable when sensible things change, appear, disappear, or contradict one another. (它让思想能够追问：当感性事物变化、显现、消失或相互矛盾时，什么仍然可以被思考？)  
**Why needed:** without a concept of being, thought is trapped inside passing appearances. (如果没有“存在”概念，思想会被困在流变的表象之中。)  
**How to use:** use it when the issue is not one object, but the condition under which objects can be said to be at all. (当问题不是某个对象，而是对象何以能被说成“存在”时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
The Greek problem of Being begins with a tension between **becoming** and **stability**. The world changes. Bodies grow and decay. Cities rise and fall. Opinions shift. Yet thought seems to require something stable enough to be named, judged, and known.  
  
This produces the first major philosophical tension:  
  
**Becoming (生成; el: γένεσις; de: Werden)** names emergence, change, and coming-to-be. (指涌现、变化和生成。)  
**What-is / Being (所是者/存在; el: τὸ ὄν / τὸ εἶναι)** names what is, or the being of what is, insofar as it is intelligible as stable. (指存在着的东西，或作为稳定者而可理解的东西。)  
  
The key issue is not whether change exists. The issue is whether changing things can be known. If everything is only flux, then knowledge seems impossible; if only stable being is real, then change becomes a problem. Greek philosophy uses **Being** to stabilize thought, but the cost is high: appearance, plurality, and becoming may be downgraded.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Being is not first one object among others; it is the horizon within which any object can be called something. (“存在”首先不是诸对象中的一个对象，而是任何对象得以被称为某物的地平线。)  
  
**Genealogical note:** later metaphysics often turns being into ground, substance, essence, or God. **Being / What-is (存在/所是者; el: τὸ εἶναι / τὸ ὄν)** becomes one source of ontology; Heidegger later reopens the question as **Being (存在; de: Sein / das Sein)**, explicitly distinguished from **beings (存在者; de: Seiendes / das Seiende)**. This distinction is central to Heidegger’s ontological difference.  
  
### 3. Physis and Archē: The Problem of Origin and Inner Order  
  
`Nature (自然; el: φύσις; la: natura)`  
**Definition:** the way a thing emerges, grows, and unfolds from itself. (事物从自身涌现、生长和展开的方式。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains order without needing every event to be narrated as divine intervention or external command. (它解释秩序，而不必把每个事件都叙述为神意干预或外部命令。)  
**Why needed:** philosophy needs a concept that names the internal principle of growth and movement. (哲学需要一个概念来命名生长与运动的内在原则。)  
**How to use:** use it when the issue is what belongs to a thing by its own constitution, not by convention or accident. (当问题是某物凭自身构成而具有何种性质，而非凭习俗或偶然因素而如此时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
**Transfer rule:** use **Nature / Physis** when the issue is inner tendency, self-unfolding, constitution, or naturalized order; do not use it as a neutral synonym for “environment,” “biology,” or “what simply exists.” (转用规则：当问题涉及内在趋向、自我展开、构成方式或被自然化的秩序时，才使用 Nature / Physis；不要把它当成“环境”“生物性”或“单纯存在之物”的中性同义词。)  
  
`Origin/Principle (本原/原则; el: ἀρχή; la: principium)`  
**Definition:** beginning, source, ruling principle, or explanatory ground. (开端、来源、支配原则，或解释根据。)  
**Problem solved:** it gives inquiry a starting point that is not merely chronological but explanatory. (它为探究提供一个不仅是时间上的开端，而且是解释上的根据。)  
**Why needed:** without an *archē*, explanation becomes a sequence without ground. (如果没有 *archē*，解释就会变成没有根据的连续叙述。)  
**How to use:** use it when asking what a thing comes from, by what it is ordered, or what makes it intelligible. (当追问某物从何而来、由何支配、凭何成为可理解之物时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
**Physis** and **Archē** work together. **Physis** asks how things unfold. **Archē** asks what principle governs that unfolding. The two terms allow Greek philosophy to move from narrative explanation to principled explanation.  
  
A myth may say: the sea behaves this way because a god wills it. A philosophical account asks: what is the underlying principle of water, motion, mixture, opposition, or order? (神话可以说：海之所以如此，是因为神这样意愿。哲学则追问：水、运动、混合、对立或秩序的根本原则是什么？)  
  
This is why early Greek thought is not merely primitive science. It invents a grammar of explanation. The world is treated as intelligible because it has principles.  
  
**Typical sentence:** To ask for the *archē* of a thing is to ask not only where it began, but by what principle it is what it is. (追问某物的 *archē*，不仅是追问它从哪里开始，也是追问它凭什么原则成为它所是者。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Physis (自然; el: φύσις)** contrasts with **Nomos (法/习俗; el: νόμος)**. Physis names what belongs to things by nature; nomos names what is instituted by law, convention, or custom. (Physis 指自然所属；nomos 指由法律、习俗或约定设立之物。)  
  
This distinction becomes one of the most powerful tools in later philosophy. It allows thinkers to ask whether justice, gender roles, political hierarchy, slavery, property, punishment, or morality are natural or conventional. The later genealogical question grows from this contrast: **what has been called natural in order to hide its historical production?** (什么东西被称为“自然的”，从而遮蔽了它的历史生产过程？)  
  
### 4. Logos: The Problem of Intelligible Speech  
  
`Logos (逻各斯; el: λόγος; la: ratio/verbum)`  
**Definition:** speech, reason, account, measure, relation, or ordering principle. (言说、理性、说明、尺度、关系，或秩序原则。)  
**Problem solved:** it connects thought, speech, and world-order. (它把思想、言说与世界秩序连接起来。)  
**Why needed:** philosophy requires a term for speech that is not mere sound, and reason that is not merely private opinion. (哲学需要一个概念来指称并非单纯声音的言说，以及并非私人意见的理性。)  
**How to use:** use it when a claim concerns the intelligibility of the world and the accountable structure of discourse. (当一个论断涉及世界的可理解性以及话语的可说明结构时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
**Usage layers:**  
1. **Strict Greek use (严格希腊用法):** **Logos (λόγος)** may mean speech, account, reasoned explanation, measure, ratio, relation, or ordering structure. Its force depends on the argumentative context. (Logos 可指言说、说明、理性解释、尺度、比例、关系或秩序结构，其力量取决于论证语境。)  
  
2. **Reception use (接受史用法):** in Latin and Christian traditions, Logos is often received through **ratio** and **verbum**, becoming reason, rational order, divine Word, or cosmic intelligibility. (在拉丁和基督教传统中，Logos 常通过 ratio 与 verbum 被接受，成为理性、理性秩序、圣言或宇宙可理解性。)  
  
3. **Contemporary transferable use (当代理论泛用法):** in modern theory, Logos appears indirectly in terms such as rationality, discourse, logocentrism, account-giving, and reason-giving. (在现代理论中，Logos 可间接出现在 rationality、discourse、logocentrism、account-giving 和 reason-giving 等问题中。)  
  
**Transfer rule:** before translating **Logos** as “reason,” ask whether the problem is speech, explanation, proportion, order, accountability, or metaphysical rationality. (转用规则：在把 Logos 译成“理性”之前，应先判断问题是言说、说明、比例、秩序、可问责性，还是形而上学理性。)  
  
**Misuse warning:** **Logos = reason** is often too narrow. **Logos = word** is also too narrow unless the context is explicitly theological or linguistic. (Logos = 理性通常过窄；Logos = 词语也过窄，除非语境明确是神学或语言学。)  
  
**Logos** is the term through which Greek philosophy makes a wager: reality is not merely encountered; it can be **given an account**. (现实并非只是被遭遇；它可以被说明。)  
  
This matters because philosophical language is accountable language. To speak philosophically is not merely to assert. It is to give a **logos**: a reasoned account that can be questioned, followed, criticized, and revised.  
  
**Typical sentence:** A philosophical claim must give a *logos* of what it asserts. (一个哲学主张必须为其所断言之物提供 *logos*，即理性说明。)  
  
**Use in reading:** when an author asks for the “account” of justice, knowledge, being, virtue, or soul, the question is usually not asking for a dictionary definition. It is asking for the structure that makes the thing intelligible. (当作者要求给出正义、知识、存在、德性或灵魂的“说明”时，通常不是要求词典定义，而是在要求使该事物成为可理解之物的结构。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** **Logos** later narrows into **Reason (理性; la: ratio; de: Vernunft)**, but this narrowing loses some of the Greek term’s range. In Greek usage, Logos still touches speech, order, measure, and explanation. In later Christian and metaphysical traditions, Logos can become cosmic reason, divine word, or rational principle. (Logos 后来常被缩窄为“理性”，但这一缩窄会损失希腊词的多重含义。)  
  
### 5. Truth: The Problem of Appearance and Disclosure  
  
`Truth (真理; el: ἀλήθεια; la: veritas; de: Wahrheit; fr: vérité)`  
**Definition:** a historically layered term for disclosure, correctness, certainty, validity, or socially authorized truth, depending on context. (一个历史分层术语，可根据语境指揭示、正确性、确定性、有效性，或被社会授权的真理。)  
**Problem solved:** it distinguishes what merely appears from what is disclosed as reliable or knowable. (它区分单纯显现之物与作为可靠或可知之物而被揭示出来的东西。)  
**Why needed:** without a concept of truth, philosophy cannot distinguish appearance, opinion, persuasion, and knowledge. (如果没有真理概念，哲学无法区分表象、意见、说服与知识。)  
**How to use:** use it when the issue is not only whether a sentence is correct, but how something becomes manifest, reliable, or authoritative. (当问题不仅是一个句子是否正确，而是某物如何成为显现的、可靠的或具权威性的东西时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
**Usage layers:**  
1. **Strict Greek use (严格希腊用法):** **Aletheia (ἀλήθεια)** can be read in relation to disclosure, manifestation, and unhiddenness, but its force depends on textual context and should not be reduced to one etymological formula. It is not merely propositional correctness. (Aletheia 可被读作同揭示、显现和不遮蔽相关，但其力量取决于具体文本，不能被化约为单一词源公式。它不只是命题正确性。)  
  
2. **Reception use (接受史用法):** in Latin and later metaphysical traditions, **Veritas** increasingly emphasizes correctness, conformity, proposition, judgment, and certainty. (在拉丁及后来的形而上学传统中，Veritas 越来越强调正确性、符合、命题、判断和确定性。)  
  
3. **Contemporary transferable use (当代理论泛用法):** in Foucaultian or critical theory contexts, truth may mean a historically produced regime of acceptance, verification, authority, and institutional credibility. (在福柯式或批判理论语境中，真理可指历史地生产出来的接受体制、验证体制、权威体制和制度可信性。)  
  
**Transfer rule:** do not treat disclosure, correspondence, certainty, and regime of truth as interchangeable meanings. Ask whether the passage is asking how something appears, whether a proposition is correct, whether judgment is certain, or how a society authorizes truth. (转用规则：不要把去蔽、符合、确定性和真理体制当作可互换含义。应判断文本是在问某物如何显现、命题是否正确、判断如何确定，还是社会如何授权真理。)  
  
**Misuse warning:** **Aletheia** should not be reduced mechanically to Heidegger’s later reading of unconcealment, nor should all later truth theories be read back into Greek usage. (不要把 Aletheia 机械化地等同于海德格尔后来的“去蔽”解释，也不要把后世真理论倒投回希腊用法。)  
  
The Greek **Aletheia (真理/去蔽; el: ἀλήθεια)** has a force that later “truth” often conceals. It is commonly read as *un-concealment*: something comes out of hiddenness into manifestation. Whether or not every later interpretation should depend on etymology, the conceptual point remains important: truth is not only correctness between proposition and fact. It can also name an event of disclosure. (真理不仅可以是命题与事实之间的符合，也可以指某物从遮蔽中显现出来的事件。)  
  
This gives Greek truth a strong relation to appearance. Appearance is not simply false. Appearance is the field in which things show themselves, but they may show themselves partially, deceptively, or incompletely.  
  
This creates a basic philosophical distinction:  
  
`Appearance (显现/表象; el: φαινόμενον; de: Erscheinung)`  
**Definition:** that which shows itself. (显现出来的东西。)  
  
`Truth (真理/去蔽; el: ἀλήθεια)`  
**Definition:** that which is disclosed beyond mere seeming. (超出单纯似是而被揭示出来的东西。)  
  
`Opinion (意见; el: δόξα; la: opinio)`  
**Definition:** belief or seeming that lacks the full stability of knowledge. (缺乏知识之充分稳定性的信念或似是。)  
  
`Knowledge (知识; el: ἐπιστήμη; la: scientia; fr: savoir)`  
**Definition:** stable, accountable, and teachable understanding. (稳定的、可说明的、可传授的理解。)  
  
This distinction is not just epistemological. It is also political and ethical. If a city lives by opinion, rhetoric can dominate. If a soul lives by mere appearance, desire can govern. If inquiry seeks knowledge, speech must become answerable to truth.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Truth is not merely what seems persuasive, but what can survive the demand for an account. (真理不只是显得有说服力之物，而是能够经受说明要求之物。)  
  
### 6. Epistēmē and Doxa: The Problem of Knowledge against Opinion  
  
`Knowledge (知识; el: ἐπιστήμη; la: scientia; fr: savoir)`  
**Definition:** systematic, stable, and accountable knowledge. (系统的、稳定的、可说明的知识。)  
**Problem solved:** it separates disciplined understanding from unstable opinion. (它把有规训的理解同不稳定的意见区分开来。)  
**Why needed:** philosophy cannot function if every belief has equal epistemic status. (如果每个信念都具有同等知识地位，哲学就无法运作。)  
**How to use:** use it when the question concerns what can be taught, justified, demonstrated, or grasped as stable. (当问题涉及什么能够被传授、证成、证明或作为稳定者被把握时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
`Opinion (意见; el: δόξα; la: opinio)`  
**Definition:** belief, seeming, reputation, or accepted view. (信念、似是、名声，或被接受的看法。)  
**Problem solved:** it names the unstable field from which philosophy must distinguish knowledge. (它命名了哲学必须从中区分出知识的不稳定领域。)  
**Why needed:** without doxa, there is no contrast that makes epistēmē necessary. (如果没有 doxa，就没有使 epistēmē 成为必要的对照项。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing belief as socially accepted, rhetorically persuasive, or merely apparent. (当分析作为社会接受、修辞说服或单纯表象的信念时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
The opposition between **Epistēmē** and **Doxa** is one of the earliest forms of epistemological hierarchy. It solves a practical problem: human beings disagree. Appearances vary. Public opinion is unstable. If philosophy is to be more than persuasion, it needs a form of speech that can distinguish knowing from seeming.  
  
But the opposition also creates a danger. Once philosophy privileges **epistēmē**, it may treat ordinary experience, democratic opinion, poetic knowledge, and practical judgment as inferior. Later thinkers will challenge this hierarchy. Genealogy will ask: who benefits when one form of speech is called knowledge and another is called opinion? (当一种言说被称为知识，而另一种言说被称为意见时，谁从这种区分中受益？)  
  
**Typical sentence:** The distinction between *epistēmē* and *doxa* is not only a theory of knowledge; it is a way of ranking forms of speech. (*Epistēmē* 与 *doxa* 的区分不仅是一种知识理论，也是一种对言说形式进行排序的方式。)  
  
**Tool-use:** when reading any philosophical text, locate its implicit version of this contrast. In analytic philosophy, it may appear as knowledge versus belief. In Kant, as a priori cognition versus empirical opinion. In Foucault, as legitimate knowledge versus excluded discourse. In each case, the Greek contrast remains active, even when the vocabulary changes.  
  
### 7. Eidos, Ousia, and Form: The Problem of What Makes a Thing What It Is  
  
`Form (形式/相; el: εἶδος; la: forma)`  
**Definition:** the intelligible structure by which a thing is what it is. (使某物成为其所是者的可理解结构。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains identity across variation. (它解释变化中的同一性。)  
**Why needed:** without form, a thing is only a bundle of shifting features. (如果没有形式，事物就只是不断变化的特征集合。)  
**How to use:** use it when the question is what makes a thing belong to a kind. (当问题是某物凭什么属于某一类时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
**Transfer rule:** use **Form** when the issue is intelligible organization, kind-membership, identity across variation, or structuring principle; do not reduce it to external shape, visual appearance, or empty formalism. (转用规则：当问题涉及可理解组织、种类归属、变化中的同一性或结构原则时，才使用 Form；不要把它化约为外部形状、视觉外观或空洞形式主义。)  
  
`Substance (实体; el: οὐσία; la: substantia)`  
**Definition:** that which is in the primary sense, or that which bears properties and persists through change. (第一意义上的存在者，或承载属性并在变化中持续的东西。)  
**Problem solved:** it gives predicates a subject and change a bearer. (它为谓词提供主词，为变化提供承担者。)  
**Why needed:** without substance, statements about things lose a stable subject. (如果没有实体，关于事物的陈述就失去稳定主词。)  
**How to use:** use it when asking what underlies properties, accidents, or transformations. (当追问属性、偶性或转化背后由什么承担时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
**Usage layers:**  
1. **Strict Greek use (严格希腊用法):** **Ousia (οὐσία)** can mean beingness, substance, essence, or primary being, depending on the author and context. In Aristotle, it is tied to the question of what is primary in being and predication. (Ousia 可指存在性、实体、本质或第一意义上的存在者，具体取决于作者和语境。在亚里士多德那里，它关涉什么在存在和谓述中是首要的。)  
  
2. **Reception use (接受史用法):** in Latin metaphysics, **ousia** is often received through **substantia** and **essentia**, which shift the emphasis toward what stands under properties or what defines a thing’s whatness. (在拉丁形而上学中，ousia 常通过 substantia 与 essentia 被接受，重心转向承载属性者或规定某物“是什么”的本质。)  
  
3. **Contemporary transferable use (当代理论泛用法):** in later theory, ousia survives indirectly in debates about substance, essence, identity, presence, ontology, and anti-essentialism. (在后来的理论中，ousia 间接保留在关于实体、本质、同一性、在场、本体论和反本质主义的讨论中。)  
  
**Transfer rule:** do not translate **ousia** automatically as “substance.” Ask whether the text is asking about beingness, essence, underlying bearer, primary being, or definitional structure. (转用规则：不要自动把 ousia 译成“实体”。应判断文本是在问存在性、本质、底层承担者、第一存在者，还是定义结构。)  
  
**Misuse warning:** **Ousia**, **substantia**, and **essentia** overlap historically, but they are not simple equivalents. (Ousia、substantia 和 essentia 在历史上有重叠，但不是简单等值词。)  
  
`Essence (本质; el: τὸ τί ἦν εἶναι; la: essentia)`  
**Definition:** what-it-is-to-be a thing. (一个事物之所以为该事物的“是什么”。)  
**Problem solved:** it distinguishes essential features from accidental features. (它区分本质特征与偶然特征。)  
**Why needed:** without essence, definition collapses into description. (如果没有本质，定义就会退化为描述。)  
**How to use:** use it when the problem is not what features a thing happens to have, but what it must be to count as that thing. (当问题不是某物碰巧具有什么特征，而是它必须是什么才算作该物时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
These concepts are tools for definition. They allow philosophy to ask what belongs to a thing necessarily and what belongs to it accidentally. This matters for metaphysics, science, ethics, politics, and law.  
  
For example, the question “What is justice?” does not ask for examples of just acts. It asks for the **form** or **essence** by which just acts are just. (例如，“正义是什么？”并不是要求列举正义行为，而是要求说明正义行为之所以为正义的形式或本质。)  
  
**Typical sentence:** A definition does not list accidental features; it seeks the form by which a thing is what it is. (定义并不罗列偶然特征，而是寻求使某物成为其所是者的形式。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** once **essence** becomes central, later philosophy can reverse it. Existentialism later makes this reversal explicit through **Existence precedes essence (存在先于本质; fr: l’existence précède l’essence)**, challenging the traditional view that essence is prior to existence.  
  
### 8. Cause, End, Potentiality, Actuality: The Problem of Explanation  
  
`Cause (原因; el: αἰτία; la: causa)`  
**Definition:** that by which something is explained as being or becoming what it is. (使某物作为其所是或其生成而得到解释的东西。)  
**Problem solved:** it prevents explanation from being merely descriptive. (它防止解释停留在单纯描述层面。)  
**Why needed:** philosophy needs to know not only that something happens, but why and through what structure it happens. (哲学不仅需要知道某事发生，还需要知道它为何发生、通过何种结构发生。)  
**How to use:** use it when asking what makes something intelligible as produced, formed, moved, or completed. (当追问某物作为被产生、被形式化、被推动或被完成之物何以可理解时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
`End/Purpose (目的; el: τέλος; la: finis)`  
**Definition:** that toward which a process is ordered. (一个过程所趋向的目标。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains processes by their completion or fulfillment. (它通过完成或实现来解释过程。)  
**Why needed:** many Greek explanations treat things not only as caused from behind, but as oriented toward fulfillment. (许多希腊解释不仅从背后的原因解释事物，也从事物所趋向的完成状态解释事物。)  
**How to use:** use it when the issue is function, fulfillment, or the good proper to a thing. (当问题涉及功能、实现或某物自身的善时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
`Potentiality (潜能; el: δύναμις; la: potentia)`  
**Definition:** the capacity to become or do something. (成为某物或做某事的能力。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains how change is possible without reducing a thing to what it already is. (它解释变化如何可能，而不把事物化约为其已经如此的状态。)  
**Why needed:** without potentiality, becoming looks like emergence from nothing. (如果没有潜能，生成就像是从无中产生。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing capacity, possibility, latency, or undeveloped form. (当分析能力、可能性、潜伏状态或未展开形式时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
`Actuality (现实性/实现态; el: ἐνέργεια; la: actus)`  
**Definition:** the realized activity or completed being of a capacity. (某种能力的实现活动或完成状态。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains fulfillment, not merely possibility. (它解释实现，而不只是可能性。)  
**Why needed:** without actuality, potentiality remains indeterminate. (如果没有现实性，潜能就保持不确定。)  
**How to use:** use it when distinguishing what a thing can be from what it is in completed activity. (当区分某物能够成为什么与它在完成活动中实际是什么时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
These terms form one of the most useful explanatory grammars in philosophy. They allow a reader to distinguish four different questions:  
  
What is it made of?  
What form does it have?  
What brought it about?  
What is it for?  
  
This grammar is not merely historical. It remains active whenever philosophy asks about function, development, capacity, fulfillment, or normativity.  
  
**Typical sentence:** A thing is not fully explained by its material composition; it must also be understood through its form, cause, potentiality, and end. (一个事物不能只通过其质料构成得到充分解释；还必须通过其形式、原因、潜能与目的来理解。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** modern mechanistic science often reduces explanation to efficient causation. Greek teleological language preserves a broader explanatory field in which purpose and fulfillment remain philosophically meaningful. (近代机械论科学常把解释缩减为动力因；希腊目的论语言则保留了一个更宽的解释领域，其中目的与实现仍具有哲学意义。)  
  
### 9. Soul, Intellect, and Life: The Problem of Animation and Understanding  
  
`Soul (灵魂; el: ψυχή; la: anima)`  
**Definition:** the principle of life, animation, perception, or self-movement. (生命、活化、知觉或自我运动的原则。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains why living things are not merely bodies arranged in space. (它解释为什么生命体不只是空间中排列的身体。)  
**Why needed:** Greek philosophy needs a term for the difference between the living and the nonliving. (希腊哲学需要一个概念来区分生命体与非生命物。)  
**How to use:** use it when the issue is life, perception, desire, movement, or the organized unity of a living being. (当问题涉及生命、知觉、欲望、运动或生命体的有组织统一性时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
`Intellect (理智; el: νοῦς; la: intellectus)`  
**Definition:** the power of grasping intelligible order. (把握可理解秩序的能力。)  
**Problem solved:** it distinguishes thinking from mere sensation. (它把思维同单纯感觉区分开来。)  
**Why needed:** if knowledge is more than sensory reception, there must be a capacity for grasping form, order, or principle. (如果知识不只是感官接受，就必须有一种能力来把握形式、秩序或原则。)  
**How to use:** use it when the issue is intellectual grasp rather than perception, memory, or opinion. (当问题是理智把握，而非知觉、记忆或意见时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
`Life (生命; el: ζωή; la: vita)`  
**Definition:** the mode of being proper to living things. (生命体特有的存在方式。)  
**Problem solved:** it gives ontology a biological and ethical dimension. (它赋予本体论以生命论和伦理学维度。)  
**Why needed:** Greek philosophy often connects the structure of life with the structure of the good life. (希腊哲学常把生命结构同良好生活结构联系起来。)  
**How to use:** use it when the issue is not bare existence, but the kind of activity through which a being lives. (当问题不是单纯存在，而是某个存在者通过何种活动而活着时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
These terms prevent Greek philosophy from becoming a merely static ontology. A living being is not just a thing with properties. It is an organized activity. This is why **Soul (ψυχή)** does not mean only an immortal inner ghost. It can mean the principle by which a body is alive, perceives, desires, moves, and understands.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Soul names not a hidden object inside the body, but the principle by which a living body is alive. (灵魂并不命名身体内部的隐藏对象，而是命名生命身体之所以为生命的原则。)  
  
### 10. Ethos, Arete, and Eudaimonia: The Problem of How to Live  
  
`Ethos (习性/品格; el: ἦθος; la: habitus/mos)`  
**Definition:** character, habitual disposition, or formed way of living. (品格、习惯性倾向，或被塑造出来的生活方式。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains why ethical life is not reducible to isolated choices. (它解释为什么伦理生活不能被化约为孤立选择。)  
**Why needed:** philosophy needs a concept for formed character and durable orientation. (哲学需要一个概念来说明被塑造的品格与持久的生活取向。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing habits, character formation, moral education, or the style of a life. (当分析习惯、品格形成、道德教育或生活样式时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
`Virtue/Excellence (德性/卓越; el: ἀρετή; la: virtus)`  
**Definition:** excellence proper to a being, function, or life-form. (某一存在者、功能或生命形式所固有的卓越状态。)  
**Problem solved:** it links goodness to function and fulfillment. (它把善同功能和实现联系起来。)  
**Why needed:** Greek ethics asks not only what rules to obey, but what kind of human being is excellent. (希腊伦理学不只问应遵守什么规则，也问怎样的人才是卓越的人。)  
**How to use:** use it when the issue is excellence, not merely moral permission or prohibition. (当问题是卓越，而不只是道德许可或禁止时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
`Flourishing/Happiness (幸福/兴盛; el: εὐδαιμονία; la: beatitudo/felicitas)`  
**Definition:** fulfilled human living, not merely pleasure or subjective satisfaction. (实现了的人类生活，而不只是快感或主观满足。)  
**Problem solved:** it gives ethics a final aim. (它为伦理学提供最终目标。)  
**Why needed:** without eudaimonia, ethical inquiry lacks a governing end. (如果没有 eudaimonia，伦理探究就缺少支配性的目的。)  
**How to use:** use it when the issue is the overall shape of a good human life. (当问题涉及良好人类生活的整体形态时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Greek ethical vocabulary is not primarily about rules. It is about formation. A person becomes a certain kind of person through habituation, action, education, and participation in a shared world. **Ethos** names the formed pattern. **Arete** names excellence. **Eudaimonia** names the fulfilled life toward which ethical formation is ordered.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Ethics is not first a theory of permitted acts, but an inquiry into the formation of character and the fulfillment of human life. (伦理学首先不是关于被许可行为的理论，而是关于品格形成与人类生活实现的探究。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** modern moral philosophy often translates ethics into duty, utility, rights, or autonomy. Greek ethical language keeps the older question alive: what kind of life counts as fulfilled? (现代道德哲学常把伦理学转化为义务、功利、权利或自主性问题。希腊伦理语言则保留了一个更古老的问题：什么样的生活算作实现了的生活？)  
  
### 11. Polis, Nomos, and Justice: The Problem of Shared Order  
  
`City/Political Community (城邦; el: πόλις; la: civitas)`  
**Definition:** the political community within which human life is organized, judged, and educated. (人类生活在其中被组织、判断和教育的政治共同体。)  
**Problem solved:** it shows that human life is not merely private life. (它说明人类生活并非只是私人生活。)  
**Why needed:** Greek philosophy treats ethics and politics as connected because character is formed within a shared order. (希腊哲学把伦理与政治相连，因为品格是在共同秩序中形成的。)  
**How to use:** use it when the issue is political membership, civic formation, law, education, or common life. (当问题涉及政治成员身份、公民塑造、法律、教育或共同生活时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
`Law/Convention (法/习俗; el: νόμος; la: lex)`  
**Definition:** law, custom, convention, or instituted norm. (法律、习俗、约定，或被设立的规范。)  
**Problem solved:** it names the humanly instituted order that may differ from nature. (它命名了可能不同于自然的人为设立秩序。)  
**Why needed:** political philosophy needs to distinguish what is natural from what is legally or conventionally established. (政治哲学需要区分自然之物与法律或习俗所设立之物。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing legitimacy, convention, law, public norms, or social construction. (当分析合法性、约定、法律、公共规范或社会建构时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
`Justice (正义; el: δικαιοσύνη; la: iustitia)`  
**Definition:** right order in the soul, city, action, or distribution. (灵魂、城邦、行为或分配中的正当秩序。)  
**Problem solved:** it links ethical order and political order. (它把伦理秩序与政治秩序连接起来。)  
**Why needed:** without justice, power and persuasion lack normative measure. (如果没有正义，权力与说服就缺少规范尺度。)  
**How to use:** use it when asking what makes an action, institution, law, or distribution rightful. (当追问一个行为、制度、法律或分配何以正当时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
The Greek political vocabulary is essential for later philosophy because it refuses to separate knowledge, ethics, and politics too sharply. A city needs truth because law can be corrupted by opinion. A soul needs order because desire can imitate political faction. Justice is not merely legal compliance; it is a structure of right relation.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Justice is not merely obedience to law; it is the question of whether law itself participates in right order. (正义不只是服从法律，而是追问法律本身是否参与正当秩序。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** the distinction between **Physis (自然; el: φύσις)** and **Nomos (法/习俗; el: νόμος)** becomes one of the deepest resources for later critique. When modern thinkers ask whether property, punishment, gender, race, sovereignty, or morality are natural or constructed, they are still using a Greek problem-form.  
  
### 12. How to Use This Chapter as a Reading Tool  
  
This chapter should be used diagnostically. Do not ask first, “What does this term translate as?” Ask instead: **what problem does this term solve in the argument?** (不要首先问“这个词怎么翻译？”而应问：这个词在论证中解决什么问题？)  
  
A compact working method:  
  
**If the text asks what something is**, look for **Form (形式/相; el: εἶδος)**, **Essence (本质; el: τὸ τί ἦν εἶναι)**, or **Substance (实体; el: οὐσία)**.  
(如果文本追问某物是什么，应寻找形式、本质或实体问题。)  
  
**If the text asks how something comes to be**, look for **Nature (自然; el: φύσις)**, **Origin/Principle (本原/原则; el: ἀρχή)**, **Cause (原因; el: αἰτία)**, and **Potentiality (潜能; el: δύναμις)**.  
(如果文本追问某物如何生成，应寻找自然、本原、原因和潜能问题。)  
  
**If the text asks how something can be known**, look for **Truth (真理; el: ἀλήθεια)**, **Knowledge (知识; el: ἐπιστήμη)**, **Opinion (意见; el: δόξα)**, and **Logos (逻各斯; el: λόγος)**.  
(如果文本追问某物如何被认识，应寻找真理、知识、意见和逻各斯问题。)  
  
**If the text asks how life should be lived**, look for **Ethos (习性/品格; el: ἦθος)**, **Virtue/Excellence (德性/卓越; el: ἀρετή)**, **Flourishing (幸福/兴盛; el: εὐδαιμονία)**, and **End/Purpose (目的; el: τέλος)**.  
(如果文本追问生活应如何被过，应寻找品格、德性、幸福和目的问题。)  
  
**If the text asks how collective life is ordered**, look for **City (城邦; el: πόλις)**, **Law/Convention (法/习俗; el: νόμος)**, and **Justice (正义; el: δικαιοσύνη)**.  
(如果文本追问共同生活如何被组织，应寻找城邦、法律/习俗和正义问题。)  
  
### 13. The Genealogical Point of Part 1  
  
The Greek vocabulary does not simply belong to the past. It becomes the hidden infrastructure of later philosophical language.  
  
**Being / What-is (存在/所是者; el: τὸ εἶναι / τὸ ὄν)** becomes one major source of ontology; Heidegger later reopens this inheritance through the question of **Being (Sein)**.  
**Truth (真理; el: ἀλήθεια; la: veritas; fr: vérité)** becomes correctness, certainty, validity, and later regime of truth.  
**Knowledge (知识; el: ἐπιστήμη; la: scientia; fr: savoir)** becomes science, epistemology, and later discourse-bound knowledge.  
**Nature (自然; el: φύσις; la: natura)** becomes natural law, essence, biological life, and later an object of critique.  
**Form (形式/相; el: εἶδος; la: forma)** becomes essence, concept, structure, schema, and formal condition.  
**Logos (逻各斯; el: λόγος; la: ratio/verbum)** becomes reason, account, divine word, rationality, and eventually logocentrism.  
  
The guiding thesis is therefore:  
  
**Greek philosophical language creates the first major grammar of intelligibility: to think is to give an account of being, truth, nature, form, and the good.**  
(希腊哲学语言创造了第一套重要的可理解性语法：思想就是对存在、真理、自然、形式与善提供说明。)  
  
Later philosophy does not simply abandon this grammar. It translates it, contests it, narrows it, reverses it, and reactivates it. That is why a quick reference must not reduce these terms to vocabulary items. They are conceptual instruments. They tell philosophy where a problem is located and what kind of answer can count as an answer.  
  
## Part 2. Latin Metaphysics: Substance, Essence, Law  
  
This chapter explains how Greek philosophical vocabulary becomes a Latin metaphysical, theological, juridical, and institutional grammar. The shift from Greek to Latin is not merely linguistic. It changes what philosophical concepts are asked to do. Greek philosophy had built a grammar of **Being**, **Logos**, **Form**, **Nature**, and **Truth**. Latin metaphysics reorganizes this inheritance around **Substance**, **Essence**, **Existence**, **Law**, **Will**, **Intellect**, and **Order**.  
  
The practical function of this chapter is diagnostic. When reading medieval, scholastic, early modern, or later metaphysical texts, the key question is not only “What does this word mean?” but **what kind of problem is this word designed to stabilize?** (核心问题不是“这个词是什么意思？”，而是“这个词被设计来稳定什么问题？”)  
  
### 1. The Problem-Situation: What Latin Metaphysics Inherits and Changes  
  
Greek philosophy asks how beings can be intelligible. Latin metaphysics asks how beings can be **ordered**, **classified**, **grounded**, **created**, **judged**, and **governed**. This produces a new pressure on philosophical language.  
  
Greek **Ousia (实体; el: οὐσία)** becomes Latin **Substance (实体; la: substantia)**. Greek **Logos (逻各斯; el: λόγος)** becomes Latin **Ratio (理性/比例/说明; la: ratio)** and sometimes **Verbum (言/圣言; la: verbum)**. Greek **Physis (自然; el: φύσις)** becomes Latin **Nature (自然; la: natura)**. Greek **Aletheia (真理/去蔽; el: ἀλήθεια)** becomes Latin **Veritas (真理; la: veritas)**.  
  
These translations do not simply carry the same meanings into another language. They reassign philosophical tasks. **Ousia** in Greek can name beingness, substance, essence, or primary being. **Substantia** emphasizes what “stands under” properties. **Veritas** tends to emphasize correctness, reliability, and conformity more than disclosure. **Ratio** introduces calculation, proportion, reason, account, and order. The Latin lexicon therefore makes philosophy more systematic, more classificatory, and more compatible with theology and law.  
  
The central problem becomes:  
  
**How can finite beings be understood as ordered by a highest principle?**  
(有限存在者如何被理解为由最高原则所组织？)  
  
This question generates the chapter’s main conceptual field: **Substance**, **Essence**, **Existence**, **Form**, **Matter**, **Act**, **Potency**, **Cause**, **Law**, **Justice**, **Will**, **Intellect**, **Creation**, and **Providence**.  
  
### 2. Substance: The Problem of What Stands Under  
  
`Substance (实体; el: οὐσία; la: substantia)`  
**Definition:** that which exists in itself and stands under properties, accidents, or predicates. (自在存在并承载属性、偶性或谓词的东西。)  
**Problem solved:** it gives thought a stable bearer for change, predication, classification, and identity. (它为变化、谓述、分类和同一性提供稳定承担者。)  
**Why needed:** without substance, properties float without a subject, and change lacks something that changes. (如果没有实体，属性就没有主词，变化也没有发生变化的承担者。)  
**How to use:** use it when asking what remains the same while features vary. (当追问特征变化时什么保持为同一者，应使用这一概念。)  
  
**Transfer rule:** use **Substance** when the issue is underlying bearer, persistence through change, independent existence, or predicative support; do not use it merely to mean “important content” or “material stuff.” (转用规则：当问题涉及底层承担者、变化中的持续性、独立存在或谓词支撑时，才使用 Substance；不要把它仅仅当成“重要内容”或“物质材料”。)  
  
**Substance** is a metaphysical stabilizer. It answers a pressure created by ordinary predication. A sentence such as “the body is warm,” “the soul is rational,” or “the stone is white” requires something to which warmth, rationality, or whiteness belongs. Latin **substantia** gives this “something” a technical name.  
  
But substance is not only a grammatical subject. It becomes an ontological subject. It is not merely what a sentence talks about; it is what can bear features in reality. This is why Latin metaphysics turns grammar into ontology. The structure of predication becomes a clue to the structure of being.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Substance is not one property among others; it is that to which properties belong. (实体不是诸属性中的一个属性，而是属性所属的东西。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Substance (实体; la: substantia)** contrasts with **Accident (偶性; la: accidens)**. Substance is what exists in itself; accident is what exists in another. (实体是自在存在者；偶性是依附他物而存在者。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** Greek **Ousia** becomes Latin **Substantia**, and this shift prepares later metaphysical systems in which reality is analyzed through subjects, properties, and underlying grounds. (希腊的 **ousia** 转化为拉丁的 **substantia**，为后来通过主词、属性与根据分析现实的形而上学系统做准备。)  
  
### 3. Accident: The Problem of Non-Essential Difference  
  
`Accident (偶性; la: accidens)`  
**Definition:** a feature that belongs to a thing but does not constitute what it is. (属于某物但不构成其所是的特征。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains how something can change without becoming a different kind of thing. (它解释某物如何能发生变化而不变成另一类东西。)  
**Why needed:** without accident, every change would threaten identity. (如果没有偶性，每一次变化都会威胁同一性。)  
**How to use:** use it when distinguishing what a thing happens to have from what it must have. (当区分某物碰巧具有的东西与必须具有的东西时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
The distinction between substance and accident is one of the most useful tools in metaphysical reading. It allows a text to say: this thing has changed, but it has not ceased to be the same thing. A person may become pale, tired, educated, angry, or old. These changes may be real, but they do not necessarily alter the person’s substance or essence.  
  
The tool is especially important for theological and juridical thinking. The distinction allows an institution, person, sacrament, legal status, or moral agent to remain identifiable despite changing conditions.  
  
**Typical sentence:** An accidental change modifies how a thing is, not what it is. (偶性变化改变某物如何存在，而不改变某物是什么。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** this distinction later supports debates about personal identity, sacramental theology, property, legal personhood, and the metaphysics of qualities. (这一区分后来支撑关于人格同一性、圣礼神学、财产、法人资格和性质形而上学的讨论。)  
  
### 4. Essence and Existence: The Problem of What a Thing Is versus That It Is  
  
`Essence (本质; la: essentia)`  
**Definition:** what a thing is; the intelligible structure by which it counts as that kind of thing. (某物是什么；使某物算作该类事物的可理解结构。)  
**Problem solved:** it distinguishes definition from mere description. (它把定义同单纯描述区分开来。)  
**Why needed:** without essence, philosophy cannot say what makes a thing the kind of thing it is. (如果没有本质，哲学无法说明某物凭什么成为其所属的那类东西。)  
**How to use:** use it when the issue is what must belong to a thing for it to be that thing. (当问题是某物必须具有什么才能成为该物时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
**Transfer rule:** use **Essence** when the issue is what makes something count as the kind of thing it is; do not use it when the analysis concerns contingent features, historical formation, social construction, or lived becoming. (转用规则：当问题是某物凭什么算作其所是之物时，才使用 Essence；若分析对象是偶然特征、历史形成、社会建构或生存生成，就不要轻易使用 Essence。)  
  
`Existence (存在/实存; la: existentia)`  
**Definition:** the actuality that a thing is, rather than merely what it is. (某物确实存在这一现实性，而不只是它是什么。)  
**Problem solved:** it separates the content of a concept from the fact that something instantiates it. (它把概念内容同某物实际体现该概念这一事实区分开来。)  
**Why needed:** one can understand what a phoenix is without there being a phoenix. (即使凤凰并不存在，也可以理解凤凰是什么。)  
**How to use:** use it when distinguishing definitional intelligibility from actual being. (当区分定义上的可理解性与实际存在时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
This distinction is one of the central tools of Latin metaphysics. It solves the problem that one can understand a thing’s **whatness** without knowing whether it actually exists. A definition gives essence. It does not automatically give existence.  
  
This distinction also creates a hierarchy. In finite beings, essence and existence can be distinguished. A creature can be understood in terms of what it is without thereby proving that it exists. But in classical theological metaphysics, God is often treated differently: divine essence is not separated from existence. God is not one being whose existence is added to an essence; God is understood as necessary being itself.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Essence answers what a thing is; existence answers whether and that it is. (本质回答某物是什么；存在回答某物是否存在以及其确实存在。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Essence (本质; la: essentia)** is not **Existence (存在/实存; la: existentia)**. The first concerns intelligible structure; the second concerns actuality. (前者关涉可理解结构；后者关涉现实存在。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** later existentialism reverses the traditional priority of essence. Sartre’s formula **Existence precedes essence (存在先于本质; fr: l’existence précède l’essence)** names this reversal of the older view that essence or nature is prior to existence.  
  
### 5. Ens and Esse: The Problem of Being as Noun and Verb  
  
`Being/Entity (存在者; la: ens)`  
**Definition:** a being, an entity, or that which is. (一个存在者，或凡是存在着的东西。)  
**Problem solved:** it gives metaphysics a general term for anything that can be said to be. (它为形而上学提供一个总称，用来指任何可被说成存在的东西。)  
**Why needed:** metaphysics needs a maximally general object-field. (形而上学需要一个最普遍的对象领域。)  
**How to use:** use it when speaking of beings in general, regardless of kind. (当一般性地谈论存在者而不限定其种类时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
`To-be/Act of Being (存在之实现/存在活动; la: esse)`  
**Definition:** the act or actuality of being. (存在的活动或现实性。)  
**Problem solved:** it prevents being from being treated only as a thing-like noun. (它防止“存在”只被当作物一样的名词。)  
**Why needed:** metaphysics must distinguish a being from the act by which it is. (形而上学必须区分存在者与其存在之活动。)  
**How to use:** use it when the issue is not what a being is, but that and how it is. (当问题不是某个存在者是什么，而是它确实存在以及如何存在时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
The distinction between **ens** and **esse** is delicate but powerful. **Ens** names the being. **Esse** names the act of being. The difference anticipates later concerns about whether “being” is a thing, a property, an act, a condition, or a horizon.  
  
This distinction also prevents a crude reading of metaphysics. Latin thought does not only classify things; it asks how beings participate in being. A stone, an angel, a human being, a concept, and God do not all “be” in exactly the same mode.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Metaphysics does not only ask what beings are; it asks how beings participate in being. (形而上学不只追问存在者是什么，也追问存在者如何分有存在。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** later Heidegger will reopen the difference between **Being (存在; de: Sein)** and **beings (存在者; de: Seiendes)**. He will make this distinction central to the “ontological difference.”  
  
### 6. Form and Matter: The Problem of Composition  
  
`Form (形式; el: εἶδος/μορφή; la: forma)`  
**Definition:** the structuring principle by which matter becomes a determinate thing. (使质料成为确定事物的结构原则。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains why a thing is not merely its material components. (它解释为什么一个事物不只是其质料组成。)  
**Why needed:** material composition alone does not explain organization, kind, function, or identity. (单纯质料构成无法解释组织、种类、功能或同一性。)  
**How to use:** use it when asking what organizes a thing into this determinate kind of being. (当追问什么把某物组织成这种确定存在者时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
`Matter (质料; el: ὕλη; la: materia)`  
**Definition:** that out of which something is made, considered as receptive to form. (某物由之构成且能够接受形式的东西。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains the substrate of change and composition. (它解释变化与组合的基底。)  
**Why needed:** without matter, form has no concrete bearer in composite beings. (如果没有质料，形式在复合存在者中就没有具体承担者。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing composition, embodiment, material dependence, or potentiality. (当分析构成、具身性、质料依赖或潜能时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Latin metaphysics inherits the Greek problem of composition and gives it systematic force. A statue is not just bronze. It is bronze under a form. A human being is not just matter. A living body is matter organized by soul as form. A legal body is not just many persons. It may be given a corporate form.  
  
The distinction is useful because it prevents two reductions. It prevents reducing things to bare matter. It also prevents treating form as a floating abstraction without embodiment.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Matter explains what a thing is made from; form explains what makes it this kind of thing. (质料解释某物由什么构成；形式解释什么使它成为这种东西。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** later modern philosophy often transforms form into structure, schema, category, organization, or system. The ancient-medieval form/matter distinction continues to operate whenever a theory distinguishes material substrate from organizing structure. (后来的现代哲学常把形式转化为结构、图式、范畴、组织或系统。)  
  
### 7. Act and Potency: The Problem of Change without Chaos  
  
`Act/Actuality (现实/实现; la: actus)`  
**Definition:** realized being, completed activity, or actuality. (已经实现的存在、完成的活动，或现实性。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains what a thing is in its fulfilled or operative state. (它解释某物在其完成状态或运作状态中是什么。)  
**Why needed:** without act, being remains merely possible or indeterminate. (如果没有现实，存在就只是可能的或不确定的。)  
**How to use:** use it when distinguishing actual realization from mere capacity. (当区分实际实现与单纯能力时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
`Potency/Potentiality (潜能; la: potentia)`  
**Definition:** capacity to become, receive form, act, or be otherwise. (成为、接受形式、行动或成为另一状态的能力。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains how change is possible without treating change as creation from nothing. (它解释变化如何可能，而不把变化理解为从无中创造。)  
**Why needed:** without potency, becoming appears unintelligible. (如果没有潜能，生成就显得不可理解。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing capacity, possibility, latent form, or developmental structure. (当分析能力、可能性、潜在形式或发展结构时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
The act/potency distinction solves the metaphysical problem of change. A seed can become a tree because it has the potency for that form. A student can become learned because the capacity for understanding can be actualized. A substance can undergo change because it is not exhausted by its present actual state.  
  
This distinction also shapes ethics and theology. Human beings are not only what they are now; they are also ordered toward fulfillment. The language of potency allows a theory of development, education, virtue, and perfection.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Change is intelligible because potency can be actualized without being sheer nothingness before its realization. (变化之所以可理解，是因为潜能能够被实现，而它在实现之前并非纯粹虚无。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** modern philosophy later redescribes potentiality as capacity, disposition, possibility, power, tendency, developmental structure, or virtuality. (现代哲学后来把潜能重述为能力、倾向、可能性、力量、趋势、发展结构或虚拟性。)  
  
### 8. Cause and Finality: The Problem of Why  
  
`Cause (原因; el: αἰτία; la: causa)`  
**Definition:** that through which something is explained. (某物借以得到解释的东西。)  
**Problem solved:** it turns description into explanation. (它把描述转化为解释。)  
**Why needed:** philosophy must say not only what happens, but why it happens. (哲学必须说明的不只是发生了什么，还包括它为什么发生。)  
**How to use:** use it when asking what grounds, produces, forms, moves, or completes a thing. (当追问什么奠基、产生、形式化、推动或完成某物时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
`Final Cause/End (目的因/目的; la: causa finalis; finis)`  
**Definition:** that for the sake of which something is or acts. (某物存在或行动所为了的东西。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains things by their directedness toward fulfillment. (它通过事物朝向实现的方向性来解释事物。)  
**Why needed:** some activities are unintelligible if only efficient causation is considered. (如果只考虑动力因，某些活动会变得不可理解。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing function, purpose, fulfillment, or normative order. (当分析功能、目的、实现或规范秩序时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Latin metaphysics preserves a broad theory of explanation. A thing can be explained by what it is made of, what form it has, what produces it, and what end it serves. This prevents explanation from being reduced to mechanical sequence.  
  
The concept of **Final Cause (目的因; la: causa finalis)** is especially important. It allows philosophy to treat natural things, human actions, institutions, and virtues as ordered toward ends. A knife is understood by cutting. An eye is understood by seeing. A political office is understood by its civic function. A virtue is understood by the kind of excellence it realizes.  
  
**Typical sentence:** To explain a thing fully is not only to identify its efficient cause, but also to understand the end toward which it is ordered. (充分解释一个事物，不只是指出其动力因，还要理解它所趋向的目的。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** later modern science often privileges efficient causation and weakens final causation. But ethical, biological, legal, and political language still frequently depend on function and end. (后来的近代科学常优先化动力因并削弱目的因。但伦理、生物、法律和政治语言仍经常依赖功能与目的。)  
  
### 9. Intellect and Will: The Problem of Knowing and Choosing  
  
`Intellect (理智; la: intellectus)`  
**Definition:** the power of understanding intelligible form, truth, or order. (理解可理解形式、真理或秩序的能力。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains how the mind grasps universals and truths beyond sensation. (它解释心灵如何把握超出感觉的共相与真理。)  
**Why needed:** sensation gives particulars, but metaphysics and theology require universal intelligibility. (感觉给予个别物，但形而上学与神学需要普遍可理解性。)  
**How to use:** use it when the issue is understanding, abstraction, contemplation, or rational grasp. (当问题涉及理解、抽象、沉思或理性把握时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
`Will (意志; la: voluntas)`  
**Definition:** the rational appetite or power of choice directed toward the good. (朝向善的理性欲求或选择能力。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains agency, responsibility, consent, sin, merit, and moral direction. (它解释行动者性、责任、同意、罪、功绩和道德方向。)  
**Why needed:** knowing the good is not the same as choosing it. (知道善不同于选择善。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing freedom, consent, responsibility, command, obedience, or moral failure. (当分析自由、同意、责任、命令、服从或道德失败时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
The intellect/will distinction gives Latin philosophy a durable grammar for moral psychology. Human beings are not only knowing beings. They are choosing beings. A theory of action must therefore explain not only cognition but orientation, desire, command, consent, and responsibility.  
  
This distinction is crucial for theology and law. If the will can consent, then responsibility can be assigned. If the intellect can grasp law or truth, then ignorance and error can be evaluated. If will and intellect conflict, moral failure becomes philosophically analyzable.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Intellect presents the good as intelligible; will moves toward or away from it. (理智把善呈现为可理解之物；意志则趋向或背离它。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** later modern philosophy transforms will into autonomy, freedom, volition, decision, or subjectivity. Existentialism centers on freedom, choice, responsibility, and bad faith, which presuppose this older problem of willing and responsibility.  
  
### 10. Law and Right: The Problem of Normative Order  
  
`Law (法; la: lex)`  
**Definition:** an ordinance, rule, or rational ordering of action. (一种命令、规则，或对行动的理性安排。)  
**Problem solved:** it turns moral and political order into a rule-governed structure. (它把道德与政治秩序转化为受规则支配的结构。)  
**Why needed:** shared life requires more than power, custom, or private judgment. (共同生活需要的不只是权力、习俗或私人判断。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing command, obligation, authority, legitimacy, or social order. (当分析命令、义务、权威、合法性或社会秩序时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
**Usage layers:**  
1. **Juridical-metaphysical use (法权—形而上学用法):** **Law (lex)** may mean enacted rule, command, ordinance, or rational ordering of action. **Ius** more directly names right, justice, entitlement, or juridical order. The two are related but not interchangeable. (Lex 可指成文规则、命令、法令或对行动的理性安排；ius 更直接指权利、正义、资格或法权秩序。二者相关，但不能互换。)  
  
2. **Critical-theory / deconstructive reception use (批判理论/解构接受史用法):** law becomes a problem of legitimacy, violence, decision, undecidability, justice, institution, and enforceability. (在批判理论和解构传统中，法律成为合法性、暴力、决断、不可判定性、正义、制度和可执行性的问题。)  
  
3. **Psychoanalytic / symbolic transferable use (精神分析/象征泛用法):** in Lacanian theory, Law may mean symbolic prohibition, separation, kinship structure, and entry into language rather than only positive legal code. (在拉康理论中，律法可指象征禁令、分离、亲属结构和进入语言，而不只是实定法律条文。)  
  
**Transfer rule:** before using **law**, ask whether the problem is enacted rule, juridical right, moral norm, rightful order, sovereign command, symbolic prohibition, or justice beyond law. (转用规则：使用 law 之前，应先判断问题是成文规则、法权、道德规范、正当秩序、主权命令、象征禁令，还是超出法律的正义。)  
  
**Misuse warning:** law is not always the same as justice, and symbolic Law is not the same as statutory law. (Law 不总是等于 justice；象征律法也不等于成文法律。)  
  
`Right/Justice (权利/正当性/法权; la: ius)`  
**Definition:** right, justice, entitlement, or juridical order. (权利、正义、资格，或法权秩序。)  
**Problem solved:** it names not only written law, but what is due, rightful, or just. (它不只命名成文法律，也命名应得之物、正当之物或正义之物。)  
**Why needed:** law can exist without being just; ius allows this distinction to be made. (法律可以存在而并不正义；ius 使这一区分成为可能。)  
**How to use:** use it when asking whether an order, claim, punishment, property relation, or authority is rightful. (当追问一种秩序、主张、惩罚、财产关系或权威是否正当时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
`Natural Law (自然法; la: lex naturalis)`  
**Definition:** law grounded in nature, reason, or the order of creation rather than mere convention. (奠基于自然、理性或创造秩序，而非单纯约定的法。)  
**Problem solved:** it provides a standard by which human laws can be judged. (它提供一个标准，用以判断人定法。)  
**Why needed:** without natural law, positive law risks becoming mere command. (如果没有自然法，实定法就有沦为单纯命令的风险。)  
**How to use:** use it when the issue is whether enacted law answers to a higher normative order. (当问题是成文法律是否回应更高规范秩序时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Latin legal-metaphysical vocabulary is not a side issue. It changes the meaning of philosophy. Greek political vocabulary centered on **Polis (城邦; el: πόλις)**, **Nomos (法/习俗; el: νόμος)**, and **Justice (正义; el: δικαιοσύνη)**. Latin vocabulary introduces a more juridical grammar: **lex**, **ius**, **dominium**, **persona**, **obligatio**, **auctoritas**.  
  
This matters because Western philosophy increasingly thinks through legal forms: personhood, obligation, sovereignty, right, contract, guilt, punishment, and authority.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Law is not merely command; it claims to express an order that can be judged as rational or irrational, just or unjust. (法不只是命令；它声称表达一种可被判断为理性或非理性、正义或非正义的秩序。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** later political philosophy, human rights theory, sovereignty theory, and modern legal subjectivity all inherit this Latin juridical grammar. (后来的政治哲学、人权理论、主权理论与现代法律主体性都继承了这套拉丁法权语法。)  
  
### 11. Person: The Problem of Moral and Legal Identity  
  
`Person (人格/位格/法律主体; la: persona)`  
**Definition:** a bearer of rational, moral, theological, or juridical status. (理性、道德、神学或法律地位的承担者。)  
**Problem solved:** it provides a concept for identity under responsibility, role, status, and relation. (它提供一个概念，用来说明责任、角色、地位和关系中的同一性。)  
**Why needed:** metaphysics, theology, and law require a subject that can be addressed, judged, obligated, or recognized. (形而上学、神学和法学需要一个能够被召唤、判断、赋予义务或承认的主体。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing moral agency, legal standing, theological relation, or social recognition. (当分析道德行动者性、法律地位、神学关系或社会承认时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
**Usage layers:**  
1. **Latin-theological-juridical use (拉丁—神学—法权用法):** **persona** may mean mask, role, theological person, legal status, or bearer of responsibility. It is not identical with biological human being. (Persona 可指面具、角色、神学位格、法律地位或责任承担者，并不等同于生物学意义上的人。)  
  
2. **Modern moral-political reception use (近代道德—政治接受史用法):** personhood becomes tied to rational agency, dignity, rights, autonomy, moral responsibility, citizenship, and legal standing. (在近代道德和政治接受史中，人格同理性行动能力、尊严、权利、自主性、道德责任、公民身份和法律地位相连。)  
  
3. **Contemporary transferable use (当代理论泛用法):** in debates about corporations, slavery, disability, animals, artificial intelligence, gender, race, citizenship, and bioethics, personhood names the contested boundary of recognition, status, protection, and responsibility. (在关于公司、奴隶制、残障、动物、人工智能、性别、种族、公民身份和生命伦理的讨论中，人格指承认、地位、保护和责任的争议边界。)  
  
**Transfer rule:** use **person** technically when the question is who or what can bear status, rights, duties, dignity, responsibility, or recognition. (转用规则：当问题是谁或什么能够承担地位、权利、义务、尊严、责任或承认时，才技术性地使用 person。)  
  
**Misuse warning:** person, human being, individual, subject, self, and legal entity are not interchangeable. (Person、human being、individual、subject、self 和 legal entity 不能互换。)  
  
**Persona** is one of the most consequential Latin terms. It can mean mask, role, character, legal status, or theological person. It allows Western thought to separate the human being as biological organism from the person as bearer of responsibility, dignity, office, relation, or right.  
  
This distinction is technically powerful and politically dangerous. It allows law to ask who counts as a person. It allows theology to articulate divine persons. It allows ethics to assign responsibility. But it also allows exclusion: not every human body has always been recognized as a full legal or moral person.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Personhood is not merely biological membership; it is a status within a moral, juridical, or theological order. (人格不只是生物学成员身份，而是道德、法律或神学秩序中的一种地位。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** modern debates about rights, slavery, citizenship, corporations, gender, disability, animals, and artificial intelligence still depend on the inherited question of who or what can count as a person. (现代关于权利、奴隶制、公民身份、公司、性别、残障、动物和人工智能的讨论，仍依赖这个继承下来的问题：谁或什么能够算作人格主体？)  
  
### 12. Creation and Providence: The Problem of Contingent Being  
  
`Creation (创造; la: creatio)`  
**Definition:** the dependence of finite being on a source that gives being rather than merely rearranges matter. (有限存在依赖一个赋予存在而非仅仅重新排列质料的来源。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains why finite beings exist at all. (它解释有限存在者究竟为何存在。)  
**Why needed:** metaphysics of finite beings must confront their contingency. (有限存在者的形而上学必须面对其偶然性。)  
**How to use:** use it when the issue is not transformation within the world, but the existence of the world or finite beings as such. (当问题不是世界内部的转化，而是世界或有限存在者本身的存在时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
`Providence (神意/照管; la: providentia)`  
**Definition:** divine ordering, governance, or foresight over created reality. (对被造现实的神圣安排、治理或预见。)  
**Problem solved:** it connects contingency with order. (它把偶然性同秩序连接起来。)  
**Why needed:** if the world is created, philosophy and theology must explain whether it is merely contingent or ordered toward ends. (如果世界是被创造的，哲学与神学必须解释它只是偶然的，还是朝向目的而被安排的。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing divine governance, teleology, history, fate, freedom, or evil. (当分析神圣治理、目的论、历史、命运、自由或恶时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Creation transforms Greek metaphysics. Greek philosophy often asks what the world is made of, what its principles are, and how its order can be understood. Latin Christian metaphysics asks a further question: why is there a world at all, rather than no world?  
  
This deepens the distinction between necessary and contingent being.  
  
`Necessary Being (必然存在; la: ens necessarium)`  
**Definition:** that which cannot not be. (不可能不存在者。)  
  
`Contingent Being (偶然存在; la: ens contingens)`  
**Definition:** that which can be or not be. (可以存在也可以不存在者。)  
  
**Typical sentence:** A contingent being does not contain the reason for its existence in itself. (偶然存在者并不在自身中包含其存在的理由。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** later metaphysics, rational theology, modal logic, and existential philosophy continue to work through this question: is existence necessary, contingent, absurd, given, created, or groundless? (后来的形而上学、理性神学、模态逻辑和存在哲学都继续处理这个问题：存在是必然的、偶然的、荒诞的、被给予的、被创造的，还是无根据的？)  
  
### 13. Grace, Sin, and Order: The Problem of Broken Nature  
  
`Grace (恩典; la: gratia)`  
**Definition:** divine gift or aid that exceeds natural capacity. (超出自然能力的神圣赠予或助力。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains transformation that cannot be reduced to natural development. (它解释不能被化约为自然发展的转化。)  
**Why needed:** if human nature is finite or fallen, natural capacity may not be sufficient for salvation or ultimate fulfillment. (如果人性是有限的或堕落的，自然能力可能不足以达成救赎或最终实现。)  
**How to use:** use it when distinguishing natural power from supernatural aid, merit, or redemption. (当区分自然能力与超自然助力、功绩或救赎时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
`Sin (罪; la: peccatum)`  
**Definition:** disorder of will, act, or relation against divine or moral order. (意志、行为或关系对神圣或道德秩序的错乱。)  
**Problem solved:** it gives moral failure a metaphysical and theological structure. (它为道德失败提供形而上学和神学结构。)  
**Why needed:** moral failure is not only error; it can be interpreted as disordered will or broken relation. (道德失败不只是错误，也可以被理解为意志失序或关系破裂。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing guilt, responsibility, disorder, corruption, or redemption. (当分析罪责、责任、失序、败坏或救赎时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
The concepts of grace and sin are not only theological. They change anthropology. Human beings are not simply rational animals seeking fulfillment. They are beings whose will may be disordered, whose knowledge may be darkened, and whose fulfillment may require more than natural development.  
  
This gives Latin-Christian thought a different diagnosis of the human condition. Greek ethics asks how habit can form virtue and flourishing. Christian-Latin metaphysics asks how a wounded will can be restored.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Sin is not merely a wrong act; it is a disorder in the orientation of will and relation. (罪不只是错误行为，而是意志取向和关系中的失序。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** secular modernity often translates sin into guilt, pathology, alienation, transgression, crime, or ideology. The structure remains: something in the subject is misaligned with a norm. (世俗现代性常把罪翻译为罪责、病理、异化、越界、犯罪或意识形态。其结构仍然存在：主体中的某物同规范发生错位。)  
  
### 14. Analogy: The Problem of Speaking about God and Being  
  
`Analogy (类比; el: ἀναλογία; la: analogia)`  
**Definition:** a relation of proportional similarity that avoids both pure identity and pure equivocation. (一种比例相似关系，既避免完全同一，也避免完全异义。)  
**Problem solved:** it allows finite language to speak about what exceeds finite categories. (它允许有限语言谈论超出有限范畴之物。)  
**Why needed:** if God, being, goodness, or truth are spoken of in the same terms as creatures, language risks either anthropomorphism or meaninglessness. (如果用与受造物完全相同的词谈论上帝、存在、善或真理，语言就会面临拟人化或无意义的风险。)  
**How to use:** use it when a term applies across different levels of being without meaning exactly the same thing. (当一个词适用于不同存在层级但意义并不完全相同时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Analogy is one of the most technical and useful tools in medieval metaphysics. It solves the problem of predication across ontological difference. When one says “God is good” and “a person is good,” does “good” mean exactly the same thing? If yes, God is reduced to a creaturely scale. If no, the statement risks becoming meaningless. Analogy provides a middle path: the term is neither purely identical nor purely equivocal.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Analogical language lets a term apply across different orders of being without collapsing their difference. (类比语言使一个词能够跨越不同存在秩序而适用，同时不取消这些秩序之间的差异。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** analogy later becomes important for hermeneutics, metaphor theory, theological language, legal reasoning, and comparative philosophy. (类比后来对解释学、隐喻理论、神学语言、法律推理和比较哲学都很重要。)  
  
### 15. Universals and Particulars: The Problem of Generality  
  
`Universal (共相; la: universale)`  
**Definition:** that which can be predicated of many. (能够被谓述于多个个体之物。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains how many particular things can belong to one kind. (它解释多个个体如何能属于同一种类。)  
**Why needed:** without universals, definition, science, classification, and law become unstable. (如果没有共相，定义、科学、分类和法律都会变得不稳定。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing kinds, concepts, properties, or general predicates. (当分析种类、概念、属性或一般谓词时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
`Particular (个体/殊相; la: particulare)`  
**Definition:** an individual instance rather than a general kind. (个别实例，而非一般种类。)  
**Problem solved:** it preserves singularity against excessive abstraction. (它保护个别性，防止过度抽象。)  
**Why needed:** without particulars, philosophy speaks only in empty generalities. (如果没有个体，哲学就只是在空洞的一般性中言说。)  
**How to use:** use it when distinguishing individual cases from universal structures. (当区分个别案例与普遍结构时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
The problem of universals is not a scholastic curiosity. It is the technical foundation for later debates about concepts, categories, social kinds, legal classes, species, gender, race, and natural kinds. Whenever a theory says “all humans,” “property,” “crime,” “reason,” “woman,” “citizen,” or “mental state,” it invokes a universal or general category.  
  
**Typical sentence:** A universal lets thought speak of many particulars under one intelligible form. (共相使思想能够在一个可理解形式下谈论多个个体。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** later nominalism, empiricism, analytic philosophy, social construction theory, and genealogy all reopen this problem. They ask whether universals are real, mental, linguistic, institutional, or historically produced. (后来的唯名论、经验论、分析哲学、社会建构理论和谱系学都会重新打开这个问题：共相是真实的、心灵的、语言的、制度性的，还是历史生产出来的？)  
  
### 16. The Tool-Map of Latin Metaphysics  
  
Use this chapter by identifying what kind of stabilization a term performs.  
  
**If the text asks what persists beneath changing features**, look for **Substance (实体; la: substantia)** and **Accident (偶性; la: accidens)**.  
(如果文本追问变化特征之下什么持续存在，应寻找实体与偶性问题。)  
  
**If the text asks what a thing is versus whether it exists**, look for **Essence (本质; la: essentia)** and **Existence (存在/实存; la: existentia)**.  
(如果文本区分某物是什么与某物是否存在，应寻找本质与存在问题。)  
  
**If the text asks how a composite thing is organized**, look for **Form (形式; la: forma)** and **Matter (质料; la: materia)**.  
(如果文本追问复合物如何被组织，应寻找形式与质料问题。)  
  
**If the text asks how change, development, or fulfillment is possible**, look for **Act (现实/实现; la: actus)** and **Potency (潜能; la: potentia)**.  
(如果文本追问变化、发展或实现如何可能，应寻找现实与潜能问题。)  
  
**If the text asks why something exists or happens**, look for **Cause (原因; la: causa)** and **Final Cause (目的因; la: causa finalis)**.  
(如果文本追问某物为何存在或发生，应寻找原因与目的因问题。)  
  
**If the text asks how action can be judged**, look for **Law (法; la: lex)**, **Right (权利/正当性; la: ius)**, **Will (意志; la: voluntas)**, and **Justice (正义; la: iustitia)**.  
(如果文本追问行动如何被判断，应寻找法、权利/正当性、意志与正义问题。)  
  
**If the text asks why finite beings exist at all**, look for **Creation (创造; la: creatio)**, **Providence (神意/照管; la: providentia)**, **Necessary Being (必然存在; la: ens necessarium)**, and **Contingent Being (偶然存在; la: ens contingens)**.  
(如果文本追问有限存在者究竟为何存在，应寻找创造、神意、必然存在与偶然存在问题。)  
  
### 17. The Genealogical Point of Part 2  
  
Latin metaphysics does not merely preserve Greek philosophy. It reorganizes it into a grammar of **ordered being**. Greek thought asks how beings are intelligible. Latin metaphysics asks how beings stand in hierarchies of substance, essence, existence, law, will, intellect, creation, and providence.  
  
The guiding thesis is:  
  
**Latin metaphysical language turns intelligibility into order: to understand a thing is to locate its substance, essence, existence, cause, end, law, and place within a hierarchy of being.**  
(拉丁形而上学语言把可理解性转化为秩序：理解一个事物，就是定位它的实体、本质、存在、原因、目的、法，以及它在存在等级中的位置。)  
  
This grammar remains active even after explicit scholastic metaphysics declines. Modern philosophy still asks whether something is essential or accidental, actual or possible, natural or legal, personal or impersonal, necessary or contingent. Existentialism later reverses essence and existence. Heidegger later reopens being against the metaphysical tradition. Foucault later asks how truth and knowledge become historically authorized. These later movements do not simply leave Latin metaphysics behind. They inherit its distinctions and transform their function.  
  
## Part 3. Early Modern Philosophy: Subject, Method, Representation  
  
This chapter explains the early modern transformation of philosophical language. Latin metaphysics had organized thought around **Substance**, **Essence**, **Existence**, **Law**, and **Order**. Early modern philosophy does not simply reject that inheritance. It relocates the center of philosophical pressure. The decisive question becomes: **how can a finite knowing subject secure truth?** (一个有限的认识主体如何确保真理？)  
  
The shift is grammatical as much as doctrinal. Philosophy increasingly speaks in terms of **Subject**, **Object**, **Representation**, **Idea**, **Method**, **Doubt**, **Certainty**, **Consciousness**, and **Experience**. Original terms should be preserved when they carry philosophical force, because key philosophical transitions are often visible in ordinary-looking words that become technical.  
  
The operational point of this chapter is direct: early modern vocabulary should be used to diagnose problems of **access**, **certainty**, **mediation**, and **method**. The world is no longer simply an ordered field of beings; it becomes something that must be represented, justified, and secured before a subject.  
  
### 1. The Problem-Situation: From Ordered Being to Secured Knowing  
  
The early modern problem is not merely “What exists?” or “What is the essence of things?” Those questions remain. But they are now filtered through another problem: **how can knowledge claim authority when inherited metaphysical, theological, and scholastic orders no longer automatically secure it?** (当继承下来的形而上学、神学和经院秩序不再自动保证知识时，知识如何主张权威？)  
  
This is the problem of epistemic security.  
  
Latin metaphysics had asked how finite beings fit into an ordered hierarchy of being. Early modern philosophy asks how a knower can legitimately claim to know. The privileged site of philosophy shifts from the structure of being to the structure of access. This is why the vocabulary of **Subject**, **Method**, and **Representation** becomes necessary.  
  
The central question becomes:  
  
**What must be true of the knowing subject, its method, and its representations for knowledge to be certain?**  
(为了使知识具有确定性，认识主体、认识方法与表象必须具备什么条件？)  
  
This generates several linked conceptual pressures:  
  
**Subject (主体; la: subiectum; fr: sujet; de: Subjekt)** answers: who or what knows?  
**Object (客体; la: obiectum; fr: objet; de: Objekt)** answers: what is known, or what stands over against the knowing subject?  
**Representation (表象; la: repraesentatio; fr: représentation; de: Vorstellung)** answers: how is an object present to the mind?  
**Method (方法; el: μέθοδος; la: methodus; fr: méthode)** answers: by what regulated path can knowledge avoid error?  
**Certainty (确定性; la: certitudo; fr: certitude; de: Gewissheit)** answers: what kind of security must knowledge have?  
**Doubt (怀疑; la: dubitatio; fr: doute)** answers: how can error be exposed and eliminated?  
  
Early modern language is therefore not simply more “subjective.” It is methodologically defensive. It is built under pressure from skepticism, error, disagreement, and the need for reliable foundations.  
  
### 2. Subject: The Problem of the Knower  
  
`Subject (主体; la: subiectum; fr: sujet; de: Subjekt)`  
**Definition:** the bearer of thought, knowledge, experience, or self-relation. (思想、知识、经验或自我关系的承担者。)  
**Problem solved:** it gives knowledge a site from which certainty, doubt, and representation can be analyzed. (它为知识提供一个位置，使确定性、怀疑与表象能够被分析。)  
**Why needed:** if truth is to be secured, philosophy must identify the standpoint from which truth is judged. (如果真理需要被确保，哲学就必须识别判断真理的立足点。)  
**How to use:** use it when the issue is not the object itself, but the position, capacity, or structure of the knower. (当问题不是对象自身，而是认识者的位置、能力或结构时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
**Usage layers:**  
1. **Grammatical-metaphysical use (语法—形而上学用法):** **Subject** may mean the bearer of predicates, properties, accidents, or states. In this sense it is closer to “that of which something is said.” (Subject 可指谓词、属性、偶性或状态的承担者。在此意义上，它接近“某物被述说之所归属者”。)  
  
2. **Modern philosophical use (近代哲学用法):** from Descartes through Kant and German Idealism, subject usually means the center of consciousness, cognition, self-relation, freedom, or transcendental synthesis. (从笛卡尔到康德和德国观念论，主体通常指意识、认识、自我关系、自由或先验综合的中心。)  
  
3. **Contemporary critical use (当代理论泛用法):** in Foucault, Lacan, feminism, postcolonial theory, and critical theory, subject often means a produced position formed by discourse, power, language, gender, race, desire, law, or ideology. (在福柯、拉康、女性主义、后殖民理论和批判理论中，主体常指由话语、权力、语言、性别、种族、欲望、法律或意识形态生产出来的位置。)  
  
**Transfer rule:** when reading **subject**, ask whether it means grammatical bearer, conscious knower, transcendental condition, social position, desiring split subject, or subjected being. (转用规则：读到 subject 时，应判断它是语法承担者、意识认识者、先验条件、社会位置、欲望中的分裂主体，还是被支配者。)  
  
**Do not confuse with:** person, individual, self, ego, agent, citizen, identity.  
  
The modern **Subject** is not simply a human individual. It is a philosophical function. It names the position from which experience is received, doubted, ordered, and judged. This is why the term becomes structurally powerful. It allows philosophy to ask: before trusting the world, what can be known from the standpoint of the one who thinks?  
  
This marks a major shift from older metaphysical usage. In Latin scholastic language, **subiectum** could mean that which lies underneath, the bearer or subject of predication. In early modern philosophy, the subject increasingly becomes the knowing center before which objects are represented.  
  
This is not a small semantic change. It is a change in the architecture of philosophy. The subject is no longer only that about which something is said. It becomes that to which something appears.  
  
**Typical sentence:** The subject is not merely one being among others; it is the standpoint from which beings become objects of knowledge. (主体不只是诸存在者中的一个存在者，而是存在者成为知识对象的立足点。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Subject (主体; de: Subjekt)** contrasts with **Object (客体; de: Objekt)**. The subject knows, judges, doubts, and represents; the object is what is known, judged, doubted, or represented. (主体认识、判断、怀疑和表象；客体则是被认识、被判断、被怀疑或被表象者。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** the subject moves from grammatical-metaphysical bearer to epistemic center. Later German Idealism will radicalize this transformation; phenomenology will analyze the structures of consciousness; post-structuralism and Foucault will ask how subjects are produced rather than simply given. (主体从语法—形而上学承担者转变为认识论中心。后来德国观念论会激进化这一转变；现象学会分析意识结构；后结构主义与福柯会追问主体如何被生产出来，而非简单给定。)  
  
### 3. Object: The Problem of What Stands Before the Subject  
  
`Object (客体; la: obiectum; fr: objet; de: Objekt/Gegenstand)`  
**Definition:** that which stands before or against a subject as something knowable, thinkable, or representable. (作为可知、可思或可表象之物而立于主体面前的东西。)  
**Problem solved:** it gives knowledge a determinate correlate. (它为知识提供确定的相关项。)  
**Why needed:** if there is a knower, there must be something known or intended. (如果有认识者，就必须有被认识或被指向之物。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing what is presented to cognition, perception, judgment, or inquiry. (当分析呈现给认知、知觉、判断或探究的东西时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
The early modern object is not simply a thing in the world. It is a thing as it appears within a relation to cognition. This is why the German **Gegenstand** is useful: it literally suggests something standing-against or standing-over-against. The object is constituted as what confronts the subject.  
  
This transformation matters because it changes the basic relation between mind and world. In older metaphysics, a being could be discussed as a substance within an order of being. In early modern epistemology, that same being is increasingly treated as an object of possible knowledge. The object is now tied to the conditions of representation, perception, method, and certainty.  
  
**Typical sentence:** An object is not merely a thing; it is a thing insofar as it is set before cognition. (客体不只是一个事物，而是作为被置于认知面前之物的事物。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Thing (事物; la: res)** is broader than **Object (客体; la: obiectum)**. A thing may exist independently; an object is a thing under the relation of being known, intended, represented, or judged. (事物可以独立存在；客体则是在被认识、被指向、被表象或被判断的关系中的事物。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** modern philosophy increasingly objectifies the world: nature, body, society, and even the self become possible objects of inquiry. Later critiques will ask what is lost when beings are reduced to objects for a subject. (现代哲学越来越把世界客体化：自然、身体、社会，甚至自我，都成为可能的探究对象。后来的批判会追问：当存在者被化约为主体面前的客体时，什么被丢失了？)  
  
### 4. Representation: The Problem of Mediation  
  
`Representation (表象; la: repraesentatio; fr: représentation; de: Vorstellung)`  
**Definition:** the way an object is made present to the mind. (对象被呈现给心灵的方式。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains how the mind can think or know what is not immediately identical with itself. (它解释心灵如何能够思考或认识并不与自身直接同一的东西。)  
**Why needed:** if the subject does not simply become the object, knowledge requires mediation. (如果主体并不直接变成客体，知识就需要中介。)
