**How to use:** use it when the issue is the mental, conceptual, perceptual, or symbolic presence of an object. (当问题涉及对象在心灵、概念、知觉或符号中的呈现时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Representation is the central mechanism of early modern epistemology. It answers a hard problem: the mind knows objects, but the object is not literally inside the mind. How, then, is the object present? The answer is: through representation, idea, perception, image, concept, or judgment.  
  
Representation therefore creates both a solution and a danger. It makes knowledge possible by mediating the object. But it also creates the possibility that the representation differs from the object. The mind may have ideas that do not correspond to things. It may dream, imagine, misperceive, or infer wrongly.  
  
This gives early modern philosophy its central anxiety: **knowledge depends on representation, but representation can misrepresent.** (知识依赖表象，但表象可能误表象。)  
  
**Typical sentence:** Representation makes the absent or external object present to the mind, but it also opens the gap between appearance and reality. (表象使缺席的或外部的对象呈现给心灵，但它也打开了显现与现实之间的裂缝。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Presentation (呈现; la: praesentatio)** suggests immediate givenness; **Representation (表象; la: repraesentatio)** suggests mediated presence. (呈现意味着直接给予；表象意味着经由中介的呈现。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** early modern philosophy becomes representational: knowledge is analyzed as the relation between subject, representation, and object. Kant later asks under what conditions representation is possible. Phenomenology later reworks this through intentionality. Derrida later questions the metaphysics of presence that often supports representational thinking. (近代哲学成为表象性的：知识被分析为主体、表象与客体之间的关系。康德后来追问表象何以可能。现象学后来通过意向性重写这一问题。德里达后来质疑支撑表象思维的在场形而上学。)  
  
### 5. Idea: The Problem of Mental Content  
  
`Idea (观念; el: ἰδέα; la: idea; fr: idée; en: idea)`  
**Definition:** a content of thought, perception, imagination, or understanding. (思想、知觉、想象或理解的内容。)  
**Problem solved:** it gives the mind something determinate to possess, inspect, compare, or combine. (它为心灵提供确定内容，使心灵能够拥有、检视、比较或组合。)  
**Why needed:** early modern philosophy needs a unit of mental content through which knowledge, error, and experience can be explained. (近代哲学需要一个心灵内容单位，以解释知识、错误与经验。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing what is immediately before the mind in thinking or perceiving. (当分析思维或知觉中直接呈现在心灵面前的内容时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
**Idea** is one of the most flexible early modern terms. It may mean a mental image, a concept, a content of consciousness, an object of thought, or a representational unit. Its flexibility is useful but dangerous. It can blur the difference between sensation, concept, image, meaning, and proposition.  
  
The problem it solves is the need for a medium between mind and world. If knowledge occurs in the mind, the mind must have something to work with. Ideas become that workable content.  
  
But this generates a new skeptical difficulty. If the mind directly knows only its ideas, how can it know that those ideas correspond to external things? This is one of the central pressures behind early modern epistemology.  
  
**Typical sentence:** The idea is the object as it is present within thought, not necessarily the object as it exists outside thought. (观念是对象在思想中呈现的方式，而不必然是对象在思想之外存在的样子。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Idea (观念; fr: idée)** differs from **Thing (事物; la: res)**. An idea may represent a thing, but it is not simply identical with the thing represented. (观念可以表象事物，但它并不直接等同于被表象的事物。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** ancient **Idea (理念/相; el: ἰδέα)** in Plato names a stable intelligible form. Early modern **idea** often becomes a mental content. This shift marks a movement from objective intelligibility to subjective representation. (柏拉图的 **idea** 命名稳定的可理解形式；近代的 idea 常变成心灵内容。这一转变标志着从客观可理解性到主体表象的移动。)  
  
### 6. Method: The Problem of a Reliable Path  
  
`Method (方法; el: μέθοδος; la: methodus; fr: méthode)`  
**Definition:** a regulated path of inquiry designed to secure truth and avoid error. (一种旨在确保真理并避免错误的受规则支配的探究路径。)  
**Problem solved:** it replaces reliance on inherited authority, habit, or unexamined opinion with disciplined procedure. (它用有规训的程序取代对继承权威、习惯或未经审查意见的依赖。)  
**Why needed:** if the mind is fallible, knowledge requires a rule-governed way to move from uncertainty to certainty. (如果心灵可能犯错，知识就需要一种受规则支配的路径，从不确定通向确定。)  
**How to use:** use it when the issue is not a single claim, but the procedure by which claims are tested, ordered, or justified. (当问题不是单个主张，而是主张如何被检验、排序或证成的程序时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Early modern philosophy elevates method because truth is no longer guaranteed by inherited order. Method becomes a substitute for lost automatic authority. The question becomes: what procedure can any rational inquirer follow to avoid error?  
  
Method does not merely organize inquiry. It creates a new philosophical subject: the disciplined knower. To know is not just to possess correct beliefs; it is to follow the right path of inquiry.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Method is the discipline of thought by which the mind attempts to secure truth against error. (方法是思想的规训，心灵借此试图保护真理免于错误。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Method (方法; fr: méthode)** contrasts with **Custom (习俗; la: consuetudo)** and **Authority (权威; la: auctoritas)**. Method claims that truth must be secured through procedure rather than merely inherited from tradition. (方法与习俗和权威相对；方法主张真理必须通过程序来确保，而不只是从传统继承。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** method becomes a model for modern rationality. Scientific method, philosophical method, legal method, critical method, and even bureaucratic procedure all inherit this early modern confidence in rule-governed inquiry. (方法成为现代理性的模型。科学方法、哲学方法、法律方法、批判方法，甚至官僚程序，都继承了近代对规则化探究的信心。)  
  
### 7. Doubt: The Problem of Error as Instrument  
  
`Doubt (怀疑; la: dubitatio; fr: doute)`  
**Definition:** the suspension or questioning of belief in order to test its security. (为检验信念的可靠性而对其进行悬置或质疑。)  
**Problem solved:** it turns uncertainty into a method rather than a mere weakness. (它把不确定性转化为方法，而不只是弱点。)  
**Why needed:** if false beliefs can appear true, knowledge must pass through a test of doubt. (如果虚假信念可能显得为真，知识就必须经过怀疑的检验。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing skepticism, methodological purification, epistemic testing, or the search for foundations. (当分析怀疑论、方法论净化、知识检验或基础寻求时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Doubt becomes philosophically powerful when it is no longer merely psychological hesitation. It becomes a method. The doubting subject deliberately withdraws assent from uncertain beliefs in order to find what cannot be doubted.  
  
This reverses the ordinary value of doubt. Normally, doubt seems to weaken knowledge. In early modern method, doubt can strengthen knowledge by purging unstable beliefs.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Methodical doubt does not destroy knowledge; it attempts to discover what can survive radical testing. (方法性怀疑并不摧毁知识；它试图发现什么能够经受彻底检验。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Methodical Doubt (方法性怀疑; la: dubitatio methodica)** is not **Skeptical Paralysis (怀疑论瘫痪; el: σκεπτικισμός)**. The first uses doubt to find certainty; the second may suspend or deny the possibility of knowledge. (方法性怀疑用怀疑寻找确定性；怀疑论瘫痪则可能悬置或否认知识的可能性。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** doubt becomes a productive philosophical instrument. Later critique inherits this structure: to criticize is to suspend what appears given and ask what authorizes it. (怀疑成为一种生产性的哲学工具。后来的批判继承这一结构：批判就是悬置看似给定之物，并追问其凭什么获得权威。)  
  
### 8. Cogito: The Problem of the Indubitable Point  
  
`Cogito (我思; la: cogito)`  
**Definition:** the act of thinking as the point from which the thinking subject becomes certain of itself. (作为思想主体获得自我确定性的出发点的思维活动。)  
**Problem solved:** it gives philosophy a point of certainty that survives radical doubt. (它为哲学提供一个能够经受彻底怀疑的确定性点。)  
**Why needed:** if external things, the body, and inherited beliefs can be doubted, something must remain if knowledge is to begin. (如果外物、身体和继承信念都可以被怀疑，那么知识若要开始，就必须有某物保留下来。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing self-certainty, foundationalism, subjectivity, or the priority of thinking. (当分析自我确定性、基础主义、主体性或思维优先性时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
**Cogito** is not merely the statement “I think.” It is a philosophical operation. The doubting subject discovers that even if it is deceived, it cannot doubt that it is thinking while doubting. The act of doubt confirms the thinking subject.  
  
This creates a new foundation: not cosmic order, not received theology, not sensory certainty, but the self-relation of thinking.  
  
**Typical sentence:** The cogito does not first prove the external world; it secures the thinking subject as indubitable. (我思并不首先证明外部世界；它确保思维主体作为不可怀疑者。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Cogito (我思; la: cogito)** differs from **Soul (灵魂; el: ψυχή; la: anima)**. Soul can name the principle of life; cogito names the self-certifying act of thought. (灵魂可以命名生命原则；我思则命名自我确证的思维活动。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** the cogito becomes a decisive source of modern subjectivity. Later thinkers will either radicalize it, as in German Idealism, reinterpret it, as in phenomenology, or criticize it, as in Heidegger, psychoanalysis, structuralism, and Foucault. (我思成为现代主体性的决定性来源。后来思想会激进化它、重释它，或批判它。)  
  
### 9. Certainty and Evidence: The Problem of Epistemic Security  
  
`Certainty (确定性; la: certitudo; fr: certitude; de: Gewissheit)`  
**Definition:** a state or quality of knowledge that excludes serious doubt. (排除严重怀疑的知识状态或性质。)  
**Problem solved:** it gives knowledge a standard of security. (它为知识提供安全性标准。)  
**Why needed:** if mere belief can be false, knowledge requires a stronger status than belief. (如果单纯信念可能为假，知识就需要比信念更强的地位。)  
**How to use:** use it when the issue is whether a claim can withstand skeptical challenge. (当问题是某个主张能否经受怀疑论挑战时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
`Evidence (明证; la: evidentia; fr: évidence)`  
**Definition:** the manifest givenness or clarity by which something presents itself as true. (某物以其显明给予性或清晰性呈现为真的方式。)  
**Problem solved:** it identifies how certainty appears to the mind. (它识别确定性如何向心灵显现。)  
**Why needed:** method requires a criterion for when inquiry may accept a claim. (方法需要一个标准，用来判断探究何时可以接受一个主张。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing what makes a proposition, perception, or intuition appear self-secure. (当分析一个命题、知觉或直观凭什么显得自我保证时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
`Clear and Distinct (清楚且分明; la: clarus et distinctus; fr: clair et distinct)`  
**Definition:** a standard of cognition in which an idea is immediately evident and sharply differentiated from others. (一种认知标准，其中观念既直接明证，又同其他观念清楚区分。)  
**Problem solved:** it gives method a criterion for trustworthy cognition. (它为方法提供可信认知的标准。)  
**Why needed:** the mind needs a way to distinguish reliable ideas from confused ones. (心灵需要一种方式来区分可靠观念与混乱观念。)  
**How to use:** use it when evaluating whether a cognition has the required clarity for certainty. (当评估一种认知是否具有确定性所需的清晰度时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Certainty is the emotional and logical ideal of early modern philosophy. It is not enough that a claim be plausible, traditional, persuasive, or useful. It must be secure. This security is usually sought through method, evidence, deduction, or the self-certainty of thought.  
  
But certainty has a cost. If the standard is too high, ordinary knowledge becomes fragile. If the standard is too low, skepticism returns. Early modern philosophy therefore lives inside a tension between foundational ambition and skeptical pressure.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Certainty is the standard by which early modern philosophy attempts to separate knowledge from unstable belief. (确定性是近代哲学试图区分知识与不稳定信念的标准。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** later philosophy repeatedly challenges the early modern ideal of certainty. Hume weakens causal certainty. Kant restricts knowledge to conditions of possible experience. Pragmatism and later analytic philosophy often replace absolute certainty with justification, fallibilism, or warranted assertion. (后来的哲学反复挑战近代的确定性理想。休谟削弱因果确定性。康德把知识限制在可能经验条件之内。实用主义和后来的分析哲学常以证成、可错论或有担保的断言取代绝对确定性。)  
  
### 10. Consciousness: The Problem of Inner Access  
  
`Consciousness (意识; la: conscientia; fr: conscience; de: Bewusstsein)`  
**Definition:** awareness of experience, thought, or oneself. (对经验、思想或自身的觉知。)  
**Problem solved:** it gives philosophy a field in which mental contents can be inspected. (它为哲学提供一个可以检视心灵内容的场域。)  
**Why needed:** if knowledge begins with what is present to the mind, consciousness becomes the site of philosophical analysis. (如果知识从呈现给心灵之物开始，意识就成为哲学分析的位置。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing inner awareness, self-relation, mental content, or the givenness of experience. (当分析内在觉知、自我关系、心灵内容或经验给予性时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Early modern consciousness is not yet the full phenomenological field of Husserl. But it prepares that field. It makes mental presence philosophically decisive. The subject does not only know objects; it can be aware of its own thoughts, doubts, sensations, and ideas.  
  
This creates the possibility of introspective philosophy. The mind turns toward itself and treats its own operations as objects of inquiry.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Consciousness is the field in which ideas, perceptions, doubts, and acts of judgment become available for reflection. (意识是观念、知觉、怀疑与判断活动得以被反思的场域。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Consciousness (意识; de: Bewusstsein)** differs from **Intellect (理智; la: intellectus)**. Intellect names the power of understanding; consciousness names the field or state of awareness in which mental contents appear. (理智命名理解能力；意识命名心灵内容显现其中的觉知场域或状态。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** consciousness becomes central in later German Idealism, phenomenology, psychology, and existentialism. Later **Intentionality** names the claim that consciousness is always about something, developing this early modern concern into a more technical phenomenological structure.  
  
### 11. Experience: The Problem of Empirical Grounding  
  
`Experience (经验; la: experientia; fr: expérience; de: Erfahrung/Erlebnis)`  
**Definition:** what is undergone, observed, perceived, or learned through encounter with the world. (通过遭遇世界而经历、观察、知觉或学得的东西。)  
**Problem solved:** it grounds knowledge in contact with particulars rather than pure speculation. (它把知识奠基于同个别事物的接触，而非纯粹思辨。)  
**Why needed:** if reason alone cannot generate knowledge of the world, experience must supply content. (如果单靠理性不能产生关于世界的知识，经验就必须提供内容。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing observation, perception, experiment, habit, learning, or empirical justification. (当分析观察、知觉、实验、习惯、学习或经验性证成时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
**Transfer rule:** use **Experience** only after deciding whether the issue is sensory input, empirical grounding, lived experience, phenomenological givenness, practical testing, or social position; these are not interchangeable. (转用规则：使用 Experience 前，应先判断问题是感觉输入、经验根据、生活经验、现象学给予性、实践检验，还是社会位置；这些含义不能互换。)  
  
Experience becomes a rival and partner to reason. Rationalist language emphasizes clear ideas, deduction, and innate structures. Empiricist language emphasizes sensation, impression, observation, and habit. Both sides share the early modern problem: how can knowledge be legitimate?  
  
The dispute is not simply “reason versus senses.” It concerns the source, structure, and authority of knowledge. If experience supplies content, how is it organized? If reason supplies form, how does it avoid emptiness? This problem will later become decisive for Kant.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Experience supplies the mind with content, but philosophy must still explain how that content becomes knowledge. (经验为心灵提供内容，但哲学仍必须解释这些内容如何成为知识。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Experience (经验; la: experientia)** differs from **Reason (理性; la: ratio; fr: raison; de: Vernunft)**. Experience provides encounter and content; reason provides ordering, inference, and principle. (经验提供遭遇与内容；理性提供排序、推论与原则。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** later empiricism, Kantian critique, phenomenology, experimental science, and psychology all inherit the early modern elevation of experience, but they disagree about what experience contains and how it is structured. (后来的经验论、康德批判哲学、现象学、实验科学和心理学都继承了近代对经验的提升，但它们对经验包含什么以及如何被结构化存在分歧。)  
  
### 12. Perception, Sensation, and Impression: The Problem of Given Content  
  
`Perception (知觉; la: perceptio; fr: perception; de: Wahrnehmung)`  
**Definition:** the mind’s apprehension of something as present or appearing. (心灵对某物作为当前或显现之物的把握。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains how objects enter cognition. (它解释对象如何进入认知。)  
**Why needed:** knowledge of the world requires some relation between mind and sensible givenness. (关于世界的知识需要心灵与感性给予性之间的某种关系。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing sensory awareness, object-presentation, or the relation between appearance and judgment. (当分析感官觉知、对象呈现或显现与判断之间的关系时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
`Sensation (感觉; la: sensatio; fr: sensation)`  
**Definition:** immediate sensory affection or sensory content. (直接的感官受动或感官内容。)  
**Problem solved:** it identifies the raw or minimal level of empirical contact. (它识别经验接触的原始或最低层次。)  
**Why needed:** empiricist accounts need a basic source of mental content. (经验论说明需要心灵内容的基本来源。)  
**How to use:** use it when the issue is sensory input prior to judgment, interpretation, or concept. (当问题涉及先于判断、解释或概念的感官输入时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
`Impression (印象; fr: impression; en: impression)`  
**Definition:** vivid sensory or affective content from which weaker ideas may be derived. (鲜明的感觉或情感内容，较弱的观念可由此派生。)  
**Problem solved:** it gives empiricism a hierarchy of mental contents. (它为经验论提供心灵内容的等级结构。)  
**Why needed:** empiricism must distinguish original experiential force from derivative thought. (经验论必须区分原初经验力量与派生思想。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing the origin of ideas in sensory or affective experience. (当分析观念在感觉或情感经验中的来源时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
These terms allow early modern philosophy to break mental life into analyzable units. Perception presents. Sensation affects. Impression strikes. Idea represents. Judgment affirms or denies.  
  
This analytic division is powerful, but it also fragments experience. It treats experience as something that can be decomposed into units, then reconstructed into knowledge. Later phenomenology will resist this by describing experience as already meaningful, situated, and intentional.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Sensation gives content, perception organizes appearing, and judgment turns appearance into a claim. (感觉给予内容，知觉组织显现，判断则把显现转化为主张。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** the early modern decomposition of experience prepares psychology, empiricism, associationism, and later philosophy of mind. It also provokes later resistance from Kant, phenomenology, and hermeneutics. (近代对经验的分解为心理学、经验论、联想主义和后来的心灵哲学做准备；同时也激发康德、现象学和解释学的反向回应。)  
  
### 13. Primary and Secondary Qualities: The Problem of What Belongs to the Object  
  
`Primary Quality (第一性质; en: primary quality; la: qualitas primaria)`  
**Definition:** a property treated as belonging to bodies themselves, such as extension, shape, number, motion, or solidity. (被视为属于物体自身的性质，如广延、形状、数量、运动或坚实性。)  
**Problem solved:** it distinguishes object-involving features from mind-dependent appearances. (它把涉及对象自身的特征同依赖心灵的显现区分开来。)  
**Why needed:** early modern science requires stable measurable properties. (近代科学需要稳定且可度量的性质。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing the mathematizable structure of bodies. (当分析物体的可数学化结构时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
`Secondary Quality (第二性质; en: secondary quality; la: qualitas secundaria)`  
**Definition:** a property understood as depending on the relation between object and perceiver, such as color, taste, sound, or smell. (被理解为依赖对象与知觉者关系的性质，如颜色、味道、声音或气味。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains why appearances vary across perceivers while objects may remain physically stable. (它解释为什么显现会随知觉者变化，而对象在物理上仍可保持稳定。)  
**Why needed:** early modern philosophy must reconcile sensory variation with scientific objectivity. (近代哲学必须协调感官变化与科学客观性。)  
**How to use:** use it when distinguishing measurable properties from perceiver-relative appearances. (当区分可度量性质与相对于知觉者的显现时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
This distinction is a key tool for understanding the early modern scientific image. The world as measured by geometry and mechanics is separated from the world as sensibly experienced. Shape and motion are treated as more objective than color and taste.  
  
The gain is scientific clarity. The cost is the downgrading of lived experience. The world of color, sound, smell, warmth, and taste becomes less ontologically secure than the world of extension, number, motion, and force.  
  
**Typical sentence:** The primary/secondary quality distinction separates the measurable structure of bodies from the sensory effects they produce in perceivers. (第一性质/第二性质区分把物体的可度量结构同它们在知觉者中产生的感官效果区分开来。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** this distinction prepares the modern split between scientific objectivity and lived experience. Later phenomenology will challenge this split by returning to the world as experienced. (这一区分为科学客观性与生活经验之间的现代分裂做准备。后来的现象学会通过回到被经验的世界来挑战这一分裂。)  
  
### 14. Causation: The Problem of Necessary Connection  
  
`Causation (因果性; la: causalitas; fr: causalité; de: Kausalität)`  
**Definition:** the relation by which one event, state, or thing is taken to produce, necessitate, or explain another. (一个事件、状态或事物被认为产生、必然导致或解释另一个事件、状态或事物的关系。)  
**Problem solved:** it gives experience and science a grammar of connection. (它为经验与科学提供连接语法。)  
**Why needed:** without causation, events appear as disconnected sequences. (如果没有因果性，事件就显得只是彼此断裂的序列。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing production, regularity, explanation, necessity, or inference from one event to another. (当分析产生、规律性、解释、必然性，或从一个事件推断另一个事件时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Early modern philosophy transforms causation. In Greek and Latin metaphysics, causation includes material, formal, efficient, and final causes. In early modern mechanistic thought, causation is increasingly narrowed toward efficient production and law-governed sequence. The question becomes: what connects events in nature?  
  
Hume radicalizes the problem: experience gives repeated conjunction, but does it give necessary connection? This question destabilizes certainty about causal inference. The mind sees one event following another, but necessity itself is not simply seen.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Causation is not merely sequence; it is the claim that one thing brings about or necessitates another. (因果性不只是连续发生，而是主张一物产生或必然导致另一物。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Cause (原因; la: causa)** in scholastic metaphysics is broader than early modern **Causation (因果性; la: causalitas)**. The former includes formal and final explanation; the latter increasingly emphasizes efficient connection. (经院形而上学中的原因更宽，包含形式解释与目的解释；近代因果性越来越强调动力连接。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** causation becomes one of the decisive problems leading to Kant. If causal necessity cannot simply be read from experience, perhaps it belongs to the structure by which experience is organized. (因果性成为通向康德的决定性问题之一。如果因果必然性不能直接从经验中读出，那么它也许属于组织经验的结构。)  
  
### 15. Mechanism and Nature: The Problem of a Law-Governed World  
  
`Mechanism (机械论; fr: mécanisme; de: Mechanismus)`  
**Definition:** the view or explanatory style that understands natural processes through matter, motion, impact, and law-governed interaction. (一种通过质料、运动、碰撞和受规律支配的相互作用来理解自然过程的观点或解释风格。)  
**Problem solved:** it makes nature mathematically and experimentally tractable. (它使自然成为可数学化和可实验处理的对象。)  
**Why needed:** early modern science requires explanation without constant appeal to hidden forms or final causes. (近代科学需要一种不持续诉诸隐藏形式或目的因的解释。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing nature as a system of bodies governed by laws of motion. (当把自然分析为受运动规律支配的物体系统时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
`Law of Nature (自然法则; la: lex naturae; fr: loi de la nature)`  
**Definition:** a regular, general, and intelligible rule governing natural events. (支配自然事件的规律性、普遍性和可理解规则。)  
**Problem solved:** it replaces teleological explanation with lawful regularity. (它用法则性规律取代目的论解释。)  
**Why needed:** scientific explanation needs repeatable and generalizable relations. (科学解释需要可重复和可普遍化的关系。)  
**How to use:** use it when explaining nature through regularity, mathematical structure, or universal relation. (当通过规律性、数学结构或普遍关系解释自然时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Early modern nature is no longer primarily a teleological order of forms seeking fulfillment. It becomes a domain of measurable bodies under laws. This is a major conceptual reorientation. Nature is no longer primarily read as meaningful order; it is increasingly modeled as lawful mechanism.  
  
The tool is powerful because it makes prediction and control possible. But it also changes the status of purpose, value, and lived quality. Purpose is often removed from nature and relocated into mind, God, or human use.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Mechanism explains nature by lawful motion rather than by intrinsic purpose. (机械论通过法则性运动解释自然，而不是通过内在目的解释自然。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** this mechanistic grammar prepares modern science, technological rationality, and later critiques of instrumental reason. It also generates the modern problem of how value, meaning, life, and consciousness fit into a mechanized nature. (这套机械论语法为现代科学、技术理性和后来的工具理性批判做准备；同时也产生了一个现代问题：价值、意义、生命和意识如何适配一个被机械化的自然？)  
  
### 16. Reason: The Problem of Order in Thought  
  
`Reason (理性; la: ratio; fr: raison; de: Vernunft)`  
**Definition:** the power of ordering, inferring, judging, grounding, or grasping principles. (排序、推论、判断、奠基或把握原则的能力。)  
**Problem solved:** it gives thought internal order and normative authority. (它为思想提供内在秩序与规范权威。)  
**Why needed:** experience alone may provide content, but reason is needed to connect, compare, infer, and justify. (经验本身可以提供内容，但理性需要连接、比较、推论和证成。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing inference, principle, method, deduction, normativity, or systematic order. (当分析推论、原则、方法、演绎、规范性或系统秩序时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
**Transfer rule:** use **Reason** when the issue is ordering, inference, principle, justification, systematic unity, or critique; do not assume that Greek logos, Latin ratio, Kantian Vernunft, Hegelian reason, and instrumental rationality name the same operation. (转用规则：当问题涉及排序、推论、原则、证成、系统统一或批判时，才使用 Reason；不要预设希腊 logos、拉丁 ratio、康德 Vernunft、黑格尔理性和工具理性指同一种运作。)  
  
Early modern reason is both cognitive and disciplinary. It orders ideas, tests claims, resists prejudice, and seeks foundations. In rationalist contexts, reason can generate or recognize necessary truths. In empiricist contexts, reason may be more limited, operating on materials supplied by experience.  
  
The crucial point is that reason becomes a court of appeal. Tradition, custom, authority, and sense-experience can all be brought before reason for judgment.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Reason is not merely the possession of beliefs; it is the power to order and justify them. (理性不只是拥有信念，而是排序和证成信念的能力。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Reason (理性; la: ratio)** differs from **Understanding (知性; de: Verstand)** in later Kantian vocabulary, but in early modern usage the distinction is not always stable. (理性不同于后来康德词汇中的知性，但在近代用法中这一区分并不总是稳定。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** the authority of reason becomes one of the central marks of Enlightenment. Later critique will ask whether reason liberates, dominates, calculates, abstracts, or disciplines. (理性的权威成为启蒙的核心标志之一。后来的批判会追问：理性是在解放、支配、计算、抽象，还是规训？)  
  
### 17. Judgment: The Problem of Affirming or Denying  
  
`Judgment (判断; la: iudicium; fr: jugement; de: Urteil)`  
**Definition:** the act of affirming, denying, connecting, or determining something about something. (对某物作出肯定、否定、连接或规定的活动。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains how ideas become claims. (它解释观念如何成为主张。)  
**Why needed:** having ideas is not yet knowing; knowledge requires judgment about what is the case. (拥有观念尚不是认识；知识需要对事实如何作出判断。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing assertion, predication, truth, error, or the relation between concepts. (当分析断言、谓述、真理、错误或概念关系时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Judgment is where mental content becomes truth-apt. A mind can have an idea of a golden mountain, but it does not thereby judge that a golden mountain exists. Judgment affirms or denies. It creates the possibility of truth and error.  
  
This makes judgment central to epistemology. Error often arises not from having an idea, but from judging too quickly, connecting ideas wrongly, or asserting more than evidence permits.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Judgment is the point at which representation becomes answerable to truth or falsity. (判断是表象开始对真或假负责的节点。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** Kant will later make judgment central to the relation between intuition and concept. Analytic philosophy will formalize judgment through propositions, truth-values, and inference. (康德后来会使判断成为直观与概念之间关系的核心。分析哲学则会通过命题、真值和推论形式化判断。)  
  
### 18. The External World: The Problem of Access beyond the Mind  
  
`External World (外部世界; en: external world; la: mundus externus)`  
**Definition:** reality as existing outside or independently of the subject’s ideas or consciousness. (作为存在于主体观念或意识之外或独立于它们的现实。)  
**Problem solved:** it names the target of knowledge beyond mental content. (它命名心灵内容之外的知识对象。)  
**Why needed:** if the mind directly accesses only ideas or representations, philosophy must explain how it knows a world beyond them. (如果心灵直接接触的只是观念或表象，哲学就必须解释它如何认识观念或表象之外的世界。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing skepticism, realism, idealism, perception, or the relation between mind and world. (当分析怀疑论、实在论、观念论、知觉或心灵与世界之间的关系时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
The external world problem is generated by the representational structure itself. If knowledge is mediated by ideas, then the world may be hidden behind its representations. The subject may be trapped inside its own mental contents.  
  
This produces the classical early modern anxiety: how can one move from inner certainty to outer reality? The mind can be certain of its own ideas, but the world those ideas purport to represent is less secure.  
  
**Typical sentence:** The problem of the external world arises when representation becomes the immediate object of knowledge. (当表象成为知识的直接对象时，外部世界问题就产生了。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** later philosophy gives several responses: realism claims that objects are mind-independent; idealism claims that objectivity depends on mind or consciousness; phenomenology suspends the naive external/internal opposition; analytic philosophy reconstructs the problem through perception, evidence, and skepticism. (后来的哲学给出多种回应：实在论主张对象独立于心灵；观念论主张客观性依赖心灵或意识；现象学悬置朴素的内外对立；分析哲学通过知觉、证据和怀疑论重构该问题。)  
  
### 19. The Self: The Problem of Identity across Thought and Time  
  
`Self (自我; la: ego/ipse; fr: moi/soi; de: Selbst)`  
**Definition:** the subject considered as self-related, identical, or continuous through mental acts and time. (作为在心灵活动与时间中自我关联、同一或连续的主体。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains how thoughts, memories, perceptions, and actions belong to one subject. (它解释思想、记忆、知觉和行动如何属于同一个主体。)  
**Why needed:** if mental life is a sequence of contents, philosophy must explain what unifies them. (如果心灵生活是一连串内容，哲学就必须解释什么统一这些内容。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing personal identity, memory, reflexivity, agency, or self-consciousness. (当分析人格同一性、记忆、反身性、行动者性或自我意识时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
**Transfer rule:** use **Identity** only after deciding whether the issue is logical sameness, personal continuity, social classification, political belonging, recognition, or imposed category; these are different problems. (转用规则：使用 Identity 前，应先判断问题是逻辑同一性、人格连续性、社会分类、政治归属、承认，还是被强加的类别；这些是不同问题。)  
  
The self becomes a problem once consciousness is treated as a field of contents. Are perceptions unified by a substance, by memory, by consciousness, by bodily continuity, by narrative, or by social recognition? Early modern philosophy opens this question by making the self both the starting point of certainty and an object of analysis.  
  
The self is therefore double. It is the point from which knowledge begins, but also something that must be explained.  
  
**Typical sentence:** The self is both the standpoint of inquiry and one of inquiry’s most difficult objects. (自我既是探究的立足点，也是探究中最困难的对象之一。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** later philosophy will divide this problem into transcendental subject, empirical ego, personal identity, unconscious subject, embodied self, narrative self, and socially produced subject. (后来的哲学会把这一问题分化为先验主体、经验自我、人格同一性、无意识主体、具身自我、叙事自我和社会生产的主体。)  
  
### 20. The Tool-Map of Early Modern Philosophy  
  
This chapter should be used as a diagnostic map.  
  
**If the text asks who knows**, look for **Subject (主体; la: subiectum; de: Subjekt)** and **Self (自我; la: ego/ipse; de: Selbst)**.  
(如果文本追问谁在认识，应寻找主体与自我问题。)  
  
**If the text asks what is known**, look for **Object (客体; la: obiectum; de: Objekt/Gegenstand)** and **External World (外部世界; la: mundus externus)**.  
(如果文本追问什么被认识，应寻找客体与外部世界问题。)  
  
**If the text asks how the object is present to the mind**, look for **Representation (表象; la: repraesentatio; de: Vorstellung)** and **Idea (观念; la: idea; fr: idée)**.  
(如果文本追问对象如何呈现给心灵，应寻找表象与观念问题。)  
  
**If the text asks how error can be avoided**, look for **Method (方法; la: methodus; fr: méthode)**, **Doubt (怀疑; la: dubitatio)**, and **Certainty (确定性; la: certitudo)**.  
(如果文本追问错误如何避免，应寻找方法、怀疑与确定性问题。)  
  
**If the text asks where knowledge receives its content**, look for **Experience (经验; la: experientia)**, **Perception (知觉; la: perceptio)**, **Sensation (感觉; la: sensatio)**, and **Impression (印象; fr: impression)**.  
(如果文本追问知识从何处获得内容，应寻找经验、知觉、感觉与印象问题。)  
  
**If the text asks how knowledge is ordered**, look for **Reason (理性; la: ratio; fr: raison)**, **Judgment (判断; la: iudicium)**, and **Causation (因果性; la: causalitas)**.  
(如果文本追问知识如何被组织，应寻找理性、判断与因果性问题。)  
  
**If the text asks how nature can be mathematically known**, look for **Mechanism (机械论; fr: mécanisme)**, **Law of Nature (自然法则; la: lex naturae)**, and **Primary Quality (第一性质; en: primary quality)**.  
(如果文本追问自然如何能被数学化认识，应寻找机械论、自然法则与第一性质问题。)  
  
### 21. The Genealogical Point of Part 3  
  
Early modern philosophy changes the grammar of knowledge. Greek philosophy asks how being, truth, nature, and form are intelligible. Latin metaphysics asks how finite beings are ordered through substance, essence, existence, law, and cause. Early modern philosophy asks how the subject can secure knowledge through method, representation, doubt, and certainty.  
  
The guiding thesis is:  
  
**Early modern philosophical language turns knowledge into a problem of secured access: to know is to represent an object before a subject according to a method that can resist error.**  
(近代哲学语言把知识转化为被确保的通达问题：认识就是按照一种能够抵抗错误的方法，把对象表象给主体。)  
  
This grammar remains active throughout modern thought. Kant asks what makes such representation possible. German Idealism asks whether subject and object can be reconciled within reason or spirit. Phenomenology asks how objects are given to consciousness. Analytic philosophy reconstructs knowledge through propositions, justification, and argument. Foucault later asks what historical regimes allow something to count as knowledge at all. Derrida later questions the metaphysics of presence that representational thinking often presupposes.  
  
The early modern subject therefore does not disappear. It becomes the problem that later philosophy must inherit, deepen, and criticize.  
  
## Part 4. Kantian Critique: Conditions of Possibility  
  
This chapter explains the Kantian transformation of philosophical language. Early modern philosophy had asked how a subject can secure knowledge through method, doubt, representation, and certainty. Kant changes the level of the question. He does not merely ask whether knowledge is certain. He asks: **what must already be in place for experience and knowledge to be possible at all?** (为了使经验与知识成为可能，必须已经具备什么条件？)  
  
This is the birth of the modern critical vocabulary: **Transcendental**, **A priori**, **Intuition**, **Concept**, **Category**, **Synthesis**, **Apperception**, **Phenomenon**, **Noumenon**, **Judgment**, and **Condition of Possibility**. In Kant and later Husserl, **Transcendental** names inquiry into the **conditions of possibility** of experience, and this chapter develops that idea into a usable philosophical instrument.  
  
The operational use of this chapter is precise: Kantian vocabulary should be used when the issue is not simply **what is known**, but **what makes knowing possible**. (康德式词汇的使用场景不是“什么被认识”，而是“什么使认识成为可能”。)  
  
### 1. The Problem-Situation: From Certainty to Conditions  
  
Early modern philosophy sought secure foundations. Descartes found certainty in the **Cogito (我思; la: cogito)**. Empiricism looked to **Experience (经验; la: experientia)**, **Perception (知觉; la: perceptio)**, and **Impression (印象; fr: impression)**. But a difficulty remained: if knowledge depends on experience, how can it contain necessity? If knowledge depends on reason, how can it apply to the world?  
  
Kant’s question emerges from this pressure.  
  
**How can knowledge be both necessary and about experience?**  
(知识如何既具有必然性，又关涉经验？)  
  
This is not a minor epistemological puzzle. It reorganizes philosophy. The problem is no longer only whether the mind corresponds to objects. The problem becomes whether objects, as objects of experience, must conform to the conditions under which the mind can experience them.  
  
This is the critical turn.  
  
`Critical Philosophy (批判哲学; de: Kritik)`  
**Definition:** an inquiry into the limits, powers, and conditions of reason. (对理性的限度、能力与条件的探究。)  
**Problem solved:** it prevents philosophy from either dogmatically claiming knowledge beyond experience or skeptically abandoning knowledge within experience. (它防止哲学一方面独断地宣称超出经验的知识，另一方面又怀疑论式地放弃经验内知识。)  
**Why needed:** reason must examine its own conditions before claiming authority over objects. (理性在声称支配对象之前，必须考察自身条件。)  
**How to use:** use it when the issue is the legitimacy, scope, or limit of reason’s claims. (当问题涉及理性主张的合法性、范围或限度时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
The critical move is therefore neither simple rationalism nor simple empiricism. It asks what reason contributes to experience and where reason exceeds its legitimate use.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Critique does not destroy reason; it determines the conditions under which reason has legitimate authority. (批判并不摧毁理性；它规定理性具有合法权威的条件。)  
  
### 2. Transcendental: The Problem of Conditions  
  
`Transcendental (先验的; de: transzendental)`  
**Definition:** concerning the conditions that make experience, knowledge, or objectivity possible. (关涉使经验、知识或客观性成为可能的条件。)  
**Problem solved:** it shifts inquiry from objects to the conditions under which objects can be known. (它把探究从对象转向对象何以能够被认识的条件。)  
**Why needed:** without this term, philosophy confuses claims about objects with claims about the conditions for experiencing objects. (如果没有这一术语，哲学会混淆关于对象的主张与关于经验对象之条件的主张。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing what must be presupposed for experience or knowledge to occur. (当分析经验或知识发生所必须预设的东西时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
**Transcendental** is the central tool of this chapter. It does not mean “mystical,” “spiritual,” or simply “beyond experience.” It means: concerning what makes experience possible.  
  
This distinction matters because Kant is not primarily giving another theory of objects. He is examining the form of objectivity itself. For an object to appear as an object, it must be given in space and time, unified through synthesis, and thought through concepts and categories. These are not empirical discoveries about one object among others. They are conditions for objects to appear as objects.  
  
**Typical sentence:** A transcendental question asks not what an object is, but what conditions allow it to be experienced as an object. (先验问题追问的不是对象是什么，而是什么条件使对象能够作为对象被经验。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Transcendental (先验的; de: transzendental)** differs from **Transcendent (超验的; de: transzendent)**. The transcendental concerns conditions of possible experience; the transcendent goes beyond possible experience. (先验的关涉可能经验的条件；超验的则越出可能经验。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** early modern philosophy had centered representation and certainty. Kant radicalizes this by asking what makes representation and certainty possible in the first place. Later Husserl will transform transcendental inquiry into phenomenological reduction, a return from the natural world to constitutive conditions.  
  
### 3. A Priori and A Posteriori: The Problem of Source and Necessity  
  
`A priori (先天的/先天地; la: a priori; de: apriorisch)`  
**Definition:** knowable independently of particular empirical experience. (独立于特定经验而可知。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains how knowledge can have necessity and universality. (它解释知识如何具有必然性与普遍性。)  
**Why needed:** empirical observation alone gives what happens to be the case, not what must be the case. (单纯经验观察给出的是碰巧如此，而不是必然如此。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing necessity, universality, formal conditions, or non-empirical grounds of knowledge. (当分析必然性、普遍性、形式条件或知识的非经验根据时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
`A posteriori (后天的/后验地; la: a posteriori; de: aposteriorisch)`  
**Definition:** knowable through empirical experience. (通过经验而可知。)  
**Problem solved:** it identifies knowledge that depends on encounter, observation, or sensory givenness. (它识别依赖遭遇、观察或感性给予性的知识。)  
**Why needed:** not all knowledge can be derived from pure reason or form. (并非所有知识都能从纯理性或形式中推出。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing empirical facts, observation-based claims, or contingent knowledge. (当分析经验事实、基于观察的主张或偶然知识时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
The distinction between **a priori** and **a posteriori** is not a simple distinction between “before birth” and “after birth,” nor between “innate” and “learned.” It is a distinction about epistemic dependence. Does the justification of the claim depend on particular experience?  
  
For example, “every event has a cause” is not treated by Kant as a mere generalization from many observed events. If it were only empirical, it would lack strict necessity. Kant’s question is whether causality functions as an a priori condition for experiencing events as objectively ordered.  
  
**Typical sentence:** A priori knowledge does not come from particular experience, but it may still structure all possible experience. (先天知识并不来自特定经验，但它仍可能结构化一切可能经验。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **A priori (先天的; la: a priori)** concerns independence from empirical source; **Transcendental (先验的; de: transzendental)** concerns the conditions of possible experience. The two often overlap, but they are not identical. (A priori 关涉独立于经验来源；transcendental 关涉可能经验的条件。二者常有重叠，但并不等同。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** the a priori becomes one of the central weapons against both empiricism and dogmatic rationalism. It preserves necessity without returning to metaphysical speculation beyond possible experience. (先天性成为同时反对经验论与独断理性主义的核心工具之一。它保存必然性，同时不回到越出可能经验的形而上学思辨。)  
  
### 4. Synthetic A Priori: The Problem of Expansive Necessity  
  
`Synthetic A Priori (先天综合; de: synthetisch a priori)`  
**Definition:** a judgment that is necessary and universal, yet expands knowledge rather than merely analyzing a concept. (一种必然且普遍、但扩展知识而不只是分析概念的判断。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains how mathematics, natural science, and metaphysics can contain necessary yet informative claims. (它解释数学、自然科学与形而上学如何能够包含既必然又有信息量的主张。)  
**Why needed:** analytic truths are necessary but merely explicative; empirical truths are informative but not strictly necessary. (分析真理具有必然性但只是解释性的；经验真理有信息量但不严格必然。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing how a claim can be both necessary and knowledge-extending. (当分析一个主张如何既必然又扩展知识时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
This is one of the most important Kantian tools. It addresses a gap in previous philosophy.  
  
An **Analytic Judgment (分析判断; de: analytisches Urteil)** unfolds what is already contained in a concept. (分析判断展开概念中已经包含的内容。)  
  
A **Synthetic Judgment (综合判断; de: synthetisches Urteil)** adds something not already contained in the concept. (综合判断添加概念中尚未包含的内容。)  
  
An **A posteriori Judgment (后天判断; la: a posteriori; de: aposteriorisch)** depends on experience and is usually contingent. (后天判断依赖经验，通常是偶然的。)  
  
A **Synthetic A Priori Judgment (先天综合判断; de: synthetisch a priori)** is both necessary and ampliative. (先天综合判断既具有必然性，又具有扩展性。)  
  
The problem is clear: how can a judgment extend knowledge without depending on empirical observation? Kant’s answer is that some judgments are grounded in the conditions under which experience itself is possible. They do not describe one empirical object; they articulate the necessary form of possible experience.  
  
**Typical sentence:** The synthetic a priori names Kant’s attempt to explain how necessary knowledge can be genuinely informative. (先天综合命名了康德解释“必然知识如何能够真正扩展认识”的尝试。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** this concept becomes the hinge of modern philosophy. It relocates metaphysics from claims about supersensible objects to claims about the structure of possible experience. (这一概念成为现代哲学的枢纽。它把形而上学从关于超感性对象的主张转移到关于可能经验结构的主张。)  
  
### 5. Intuition: The Problem of Givenness  
  
`Intuition (直观; de: Anschauung)`  
**Definition:** the immediate way in which objects are given to sensibility. (对象被直接给予感性的方式。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains how cognition receives singular content. (它解释认知如何获得个别内容。)  
**Why needed:** concepts alone cannot produce objects; cognition requires something given. (单靠概念不能产生对象；认知需要某种被给予之物。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing the immediate givenness of objects in space and time. (当分析对象在空间与时间中的直接给予性时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Kantian **Intuition** does not mean a vague hunch. It means immediate singular givenness. Concepts are general; intuitions are singular. A concept such as “tree” can apply to many trees. An intuition gives this tree here and now.  
  
This distinction prevents two errors. First, it prevents rationalism from thinking that concepts alone can generate knowledge of objects. Second, it prevents empiricism from treating sensory data as already organized knowledge. Intuition gives material, but it must be structured.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Intuition gives objects immediately; concepts make them thinkable. (直观直接给予对象；概念使对象成为可思者。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Intuition (直观; de: Anschauung)** contrasts with **Concept (概念; de: Begriff)**. Intuition is singular and immediate; concept is general and mediate. (直观是个别的、直接的；概念是普遍的、中介性的。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** Kant’s concept of intuition prepares later debates about givenness, perception, phenomenology, and the relation between sensibility and conceptuality. (康德的直观概念为后来的给予性、知觉、现象学以及感性与概念性关系之争做准备。)  
  
### 6. Sensibility: The Problem of Receptivity  
  
`Sensibility (感性; de: Sinnlichkeit)`  
**Definition:** the receptive capacity through which objects are given. (对象借以被给予的接受性能力。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains the mind’s dependence on being affected. (它解释心灵依赖受动性的方面。)  
**Why needed:** finite cognition cannot create its objects merely by thinking them. (有限认知不能仅通过思维创造其对象。)  
**How to use:** use it when the issue is receptivity, affection, sensory givenness, or the form of appearance. (当问题涉及接受性、受动、感性给予性或显现形式时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Sensibility is Kant’s answer to a limitation of finite knowledge. Human beings are not divine intellects that create objects by thinking them. They must be affected. Objects must be given. Sensibility is the faculty of receiving this givenness.  
  
But sensibility is not chaotic raw material. It has forms. These forms are **Space (空间; de: Raum)** and **Time (时间; de: Zeit)**. They are not learned from experience as ordinary empirical concepts. They are the forms through which outer and inner appearances are possible.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Sensibility is receptive, but its receptivity is already structured by space and time. (感性是接受性的，但其接受性已经由空间与时间所结构化。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** sensibility becomes a way to preserve the dependence of knowledge on givenness while denying that experience is formless. (感性概念保存了知识对给予性的依赖，同时否认经验是无形式的。)  
  
### 7. Space and Time: The Problem of the Form of Appearance  
  
`Space (空间; de: Raum)`  
**Definition:** the a priori form of outer intuition. (外直观的先天形式。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains how outer objects can appear as outside one another and ordered spatially. (它解释外部对象如何能够作为彼此外在并按空间秩序显现。)  
**Why needed:** spatial order cannot be abstracted from experience unless experience is already spatially ordered. (如果经验不是已经被空间化地组织，空间秩序就无法从经验中抽象出来。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing the condition under which outer appearances are possible. (当分析外部显现何以可能的条件时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
`Time (时间; de: Zeit)`  
**Definition:** the a priori form of inner intuition and the universal form of all appearances. (内直观的先天形式，也是一切显现的普遍形式。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains succession, simultaneity, duration, and inner experience. (它解释连续、同时、持续与内在经验。)  
**Why needed:** experience requires temporal order before events can be represented as before, after, or simultaneous. (经验需要时间秩序，事件才能被表象为先后或同时。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing the condition under which inner and outer appearances are temporally ordered. (当分析内外显现如何被时间性地组织时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Space and time are not containers discovered by looking around. They are forms of intuition. This means they structure how objects can appear to us. We do not first encounter non-spatial data and then add space. Outer appearance is already spatial. We do not first encounter unordered events and then add time. Experience is already temporal.  
  
This is a key Kantian move: what seems to belong simply to the world may belong to the form under which the world can appear to finite knowers.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Space and time are not empirical things but forms under which things can appear. (空间与时间不是经验对象，而是事物得以显现的形式。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Space and Time (空间与时间; de: Raum und Zeit)** are empirically real but transcendentally ideal. They are valid for all possible experience, but they are not things in themselves. (空间与时间在经验上实在，但在先验上观念；它们对一切可能经验有效，但不是物自身。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** this move transforms metaphysics. Instead of asking whether space and time are absolute external realities or mere relations among things, Kant asks what role they play in making experience possible. (这一转变改造了形而上学。康德不再只问空间与时间是绝对外部实在还是事物间关系，而是问它们在使经验成为可能中起什么作用。)  
  
### 8. Concept: The Problem of Thinking the Given  
  
`Concept (概念; de: Begriff)`  
**Definition:** a general representation through which intuitions are thought and unified. (一种普遍表象，直观通过它被思考并统一。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains how given content becomes intelligible as something. (它解释被给予的内容如何作为某物而成为可理解的。)  
**Why needed:** intuitions without concepts are blind; givenness without thinking does not yet yield knowledge. (没有概念的直观是盲的；没有思维的给予性尚未产生知识。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing classification, judgment, rule, unity, or generality in cognition. (当分析分类、判断、规则、统一性或认知中的普遍性时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
A concept does not merely label an object after the fact. It functions as a rule for unifying manifold intuition. To recognize something as a tree, body, cause, event, or substance is already to bring the manifold under a concept.  
  
This is why Kantian knowledge requires both intuition and concept. Intuition gives content. Concept gives unity and thinkability.  
  
**Typical sentence:** A concept is not a mental picture; it is a rule for thinking the manifold as one object or kind. (概念不是心灵图像，而是把杂多作为一个对象或种类来思考的规则。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Intuition (直观; de: Anschauung)** without **Concept (概念; de: Begriff)** is blind; **Concept** without **Intuition** is empty. (没有概念的直观是盲的；没有直观的概念是空的。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** the concept becomes a mediating tool between raw empiricism and pure rationalism. Later German Idealism will make the concept dynamic and historical; analytic philosophy will treat concepts through definition, reference, and logical role. (概念成为介于原始经验论与纯粹理性主义之间的中介工具。后来德国观念论会使概念动态化、历史化；分析哲学会通过定义、指称和逻辑角色处理概念。)  
  
### 9. Understanding: The Problem of Rule-Governed Unity  
  
`Understanding (知性; de: Verstand)`  
**Definition:** the faculty of concepts, rules, and judgments. (概念、规则和判断的能力。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains how sensory manifold becomes unified under concepts. (它解释感性杂多如何在概念下被统一。)  
**Why needed:** sensibility gives manifold content, but knowledge requires rule-governed unity. (感性给予杂多内容，但知识需要受规则支配的统一性。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing conceptual ordering, judgment, category-use, or objective cognition. (当分析概念排序、判断、范畴使用或客观认知时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Understanding is not the same as reason in Kant’s strict vocabulary. **Understanding** gives rules and applies concepts to intuition. **Reason** seeks higher unity, principles, and the unconditioned. This distinction is crucial because Kant wants to show both the legitimate use and illegitimate overreach of cognition.  
  
Understanding is legitimate when it structures possible experience. It becomes problematic only when concepts are used beyond any possible intuition.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Understanding supplies rules through which the manifold of intuition can be thought as an object. (知性提供规则，通过这些规则，直观杂多能够被思考为对象。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Understanding (知性; de: Verstand)** differs from **Reason (理性; de: Vernunft)**. Understanding organizes experience through concepts; reason seeks systematic unity and the unconditioned. (知性通过概念组织经验；理性寻求系统统一性与无条件者。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** this distinction becomes fundamental for post-Kantian philosophy. Later thinkers will debate whether reason can legitimately overcome the limits Kant imposes on it. (这一区分成为后康德哲学的基础。后来的思想家会争论理性能否合法地克服康德为其设定的限度。)  
  
### 10. Category: The Problem of Objective Structure  
  
`Category (范畴; el: κατηγορία; de: Kategorie)`  
**Definition:** a pure concept of the understanding that structures possible experience. (结构化可能经验的知性纯概念。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains how objects can be experienced as unified, causal, substantial, plural, possible, actual, or necessary. (它解释对象如何能够被经验为统一的、因果性的、实体性的、复多的、可能的、现实的或必然的。)  
**Why needed:** sensory givenness alone does not yield objectivity. (单纯感性给予性不能产生客观性。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing the most general conceptual conditions under which objects can be experienced. (当分析对象得以被经验的最普遍概念条件时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Categories are not empirical classifications such as “dog,” “tree,” or “planet.” They are pure concepts such as unity, plurality, causality, substance, possibility, actuality, and necessity. They do not come from experience in the ordinary way; they are conditions for experience having objective form.  
  
The category of causality is especially important. Hume had shown that necessary connection is not simply given in sensory experience. Kant responds by arguing that causality is a category through which events are experienced as objectively ordered in time.  
  
**Typical sentence:** A category is not learned from objects; it is a condition under which objects can be experienced as objects. (范畴不是从对象中学得的，而是对象能够作为对象被经验的条件。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Empirical Concept (经验概念; de: empirischer Begriff)** is derived from experience; **Category (范畴; de: Kategorie)** structures possible experience. (经验概念源自经验；范畴结构化可能经验。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** categories transform metaphysics from a doctrine of being into an inquiry into the forms of objectivity. (范畴把形而上学从存在论教义转化为对客观性形式的探究。)  
  
### 11. Synthesis: The Problem of Unity from Manifold  
  
`Synthesis (综合; de: Synthesis)`  
**Definition:** the act of combining a manifold into unity. (把杂多结合为统一体的活动。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains how scattered givenness becomes one experience of one object. (它解释分散的给予性如何成为对一个对象的统一经验。)  
**Why needed:** experience gives manifold elements, but knowledge requires unity. (经验给予杂多要素，但知识需要统一性。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing combination, unification, temporal ordering, or the formation of objectivity. (当分析结合、统一、时间排序或客观性的形成时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Synthesis is the hidden labor of cognition. Sensibility gives a manifold. Understanding supplies concepts and categories. But something must combine the manifold into a unified object of experience. This is synthesis.  
  
This tool is indispensable because it prevents knowledge from being imagined as passive reception. The mind does not merely receive finished objects. It actively combines, orders, and unifies what is given according to rules.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Synthesis is the activity by which the manifold of intuition is combined into the unity of experience. (综合是直观杂多被结合为经验统一性的活动。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Manifold (杂多; de: Mannigfaltige)** names the plurality of given elements; **Synthesis (综合; de: Synthesis)** names the combining activity that unifies them. (杂多命名被给予要素的复多性；综合命名统一这些要素的结合活动。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** synthesis prepares German Idealism’s more active conception of subjectivity. If objectivity depends on synthetic activity, then subjectivity is not a passive mirror but an organizing power. (综合为德国观念论更主动的主体性概念做准备。如果客观性依赖综合活动，那么主体性就不是被动镜子，而是一种组织力量。)  
  
### 12. Imagination and Schema: The Problem of Mediation between Intuition and Concept  
  
`Imagination (想象力; de: Einbildungskraft)`  
**Definition:** the faculty that mediates between sensibility and understanding by forming and synthesizing representations. (通过形成和综合表象，在感性与知性之间进行中介的能力。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains how intuitions and concepts can be connected. (它解释直观与概念如何能够连接。)  
**Why needed:** intuitions are singular and sensory; concepts are general and intellectual. Something must mediate between them. (直观是个别且感性的；概念是普遍且知性的。二者之间必须有中介。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing the transition from sensory manifold to conceptual unity. (当分析从感性杂多到概念统一的过渡时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
`Schema (图型; el: σχῆμα; de: Schema)`  
**Definition:** a rule or temporal determination that mediates between a pure concept and intuition. (在纯概念与直观之间起中介作用的规则或时间规定。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains how pure categories can apply to sensible appearances. (它解释纯范畴如何能够应用于感性显现。)  
**Why needed:** without schemata, categories would remain too abstract to structure intuition. (如果没有图型，范畴就会过于抽象，无法结构化直观。)  
**How to use:** use it when the issue is how a general concept becomes applicable to temporal experience. (当问题是一般概念如何能够应用于时间性经验时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
The schematism is one of the most difficult but important Kantian tools. The problem is simple: how can a pure concept such as causality apply to something given in time? The answer is that a schema gives a temporal rule. Causality, for example, involves succession according to a rule.  
  
**Typical sentence:** A schema is the mediating rule that allows a pure concept to be applied to sensible experience. (图型是使纯概念能够应用于感性经验的中介规则。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** the problem of mediation between concept and intuition reappears in later philosophy as the problem of application, embodiment, interpretation, model, paradigm, and form of life. (概念与直观之间的中介问题后来以应用、具身、解释、模型、范式和生活形式等问题重新出现。)  
  
### 13. Apperception: The Problem of the Unity of Consciousness  
  
`Apperception (统觉; de: Apperzeption)`  
**Definition:** self-conscious unity through which representations can belong to one subject. (诸表象能够属于同一主体的自我意识统一性。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains how multiple representations can be mine within one unified consciousness. (它解释多个表象如何能在一个统一意识中成为“我的”。)  
**Why needed:** without unity of consciousness, there would be no unified experience or objectivity. (如果没有意识统一性，就不会有统一经验或客观性。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing self-consciousness as a condition for experience rather than as an empirical object. (当把自我意识作为经验条件而非经验对象来分析时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
The **Transcendental Unity of Apperception (先验统觉统一; de: transzendentale Einheit der Apperzeption)** is one of Kant’s deepest tools. It does not mean a psychological observation that “I happen to feel unified.” It means that representations must be able to belong to one “I think” if they are to be part of one experience.  
  
This makes self-consciousness a condition of objectivity. The object is unified because the manifold is synthesized under rules, and this synthesis must be related to a unified consciousness.  
  
**Typical sentence:** The “I think” must be able to accompany all my representations. (“我思”必须能够伴随我的一切表象。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Empirical Self (经验自我; de: empirisches Ich)** is the self as experienced in inner sense; **Transcendental Apperception (先验统觉; de: transzendentale Apperzeption)** is the formal unity required for experience. (经验自我是内感中被经验到的自我；先验统觉则是经验所需的形式统一性。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** this concept prepares German Idealism’s transformation of the subject into an active principle of synthesis, recognition, and history. (这一概念为德国观念论把主体转化为综合、承认和历史的主动原则做准备。)  
  
### 14. Objectivity: The Problem of Valid Experience  
  
`Objectivity (客观性; de: Objektivität/Gegenständlichkeit)`  
**Definition:** the validity of experience as experience of an object governed by rules. (作为受规则支配之对象经验的有效性。)  
**Problem solved:** it distinguishes private sequence of impressions from experience of an objective world. (它把私人印象序列同对客观世界的经验区分开来。)  
**Why needed:** knowledge requires more than inner association; it requires rule-governed object-reference. (知识不只是内在联想；它需要受规则支配的对象指涉。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing how representations become valid as knowledge of objects. (当分析表象如何作为对象知识而具有有效性时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Kantian objectivity does not mean access to things as they are apart from all conditions of experience. It means validity under the conditions of possible experience. An objective event is not merely a subjective sequence of perceptions. It is ordered by rules such as causality.  
  
For example, seeing the sun shine and then the stone warm is not yet objective causal knowledge. The sequence must be determined according to a rule: the sun’s heat causes the stone to become warm. Objectivity requires lawful ordering.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Objectivity is not bare externality; it is rule-governed validity within possible experience. (客观性不是单纯外在性，而是可能经验内部受规则支配的有效性。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** Kant relocates objectivity from mind-independent things alone to the rule-governed structure of possible experience. Later debates about realism, idealism, phenomenology, and social objectivity will repeatedly return to this move. (康德把客观性从单纯独立于心灵的事物，转移到可能经验的规则化结构中。)  
  
### 15. Phenomenon and Noumenon: The Problem of Limits  
  
`Noumenon (智思物/本体; el: νοούμενον; de: Noumenon)`  
**Definition:** an object of thought considered apart from sensible intuition; in Kant, primarily a limiting concept that marks the boundary of possible experience. (脱离感性直观而被思考的对象；在康德那里，它主要是标明可能经验边界的限制性概念。)  
**Problem solved:** it prevents human knowledge from claiming absolute access to things beyond the conditions of possible experience. (它防止人类知识声称绝对通达可能经验条件之外的对象。)  
**Why needed:** critique needs a boundary concept that shows where legitimate cognition stops. (批判哲学需要一个边界概念来说明合法认识在哪里停止。)  
**How to use:** use it when distinguishing what can be experienced from what can only be thought as beyond possible experience. (当区分能够被经验认识之物与只能被思为超出可能经验之物时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
`Thing-in-itself (物自身; de: Ding an sich)`  
**Definition:** a thing considered independently of the human conditions under which it appears to us. (摆脱人类显现条件而被考虑的事物。)  
**Problem solved:** it marks the difference between things as they appear and things considered independently of our mode of cognition. (它标明作为显现的事物与独立于认识方式而被考虑的事物之间的差异。)  
**How to use:** use it when the issue is not an unknown object inside experience, but the limit of experience itself. (当问题不是经验内部的未知对象，而是经验本身的限度时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
This is one of Kant’s most important distinctions. The world known by science is not illusion. Phenomena are empirically real. But they are known under the forms of human cognition. Things in themselves are not objects that science has not yet discovered. They are what things may be apart from the conditions under which they appear to us.  
  
**Typical sentence:** We know objects as appearances, not as things in themselves. (我们认识对象作为现象，而不是作为物自身。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Appearance (现象; de: Erscheinung)** is not mere illusion. It is the legitimate object of possible experience. **Thing-in-itself (物自身; de: Ding an sich)** is not an unknown object inside experience, but a limit to experience. (现象不是单纯幻象，而是可能经验的合法对象。物自身不是经验内部的未知对象，而是经验的限度。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** the phenomenon/noumenon distinction turns metaphysics into critique. Philosophy must now ask where knowledge is legitimate and where reason overreaches. (现象/物自身区分把形而上学转化为批判。哲学必须追问知识在哪里合法，以及理性在哪里越界。)  
  
### 16. Reason and Ideas: The Problem of the Unconditioned  
  
`Reason (理性; de: Vernunft)`  
**Definition:** the faculty that seeks principles, systematic unity, and the unconditioned. (寻求原则、系统统一性与无条件者的能力。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains why human thought moves beyond isolated empirical judgments toward totality, ground, and ultimate explanation. (它解释人类思想为何会越出孤立经验判断，趋向总体、根据和终极解释。)  
**Why needed:** understanding organizes experience, but reason seeks the highest unity of that organization. (知性组织经验，但理性寻求这种组织的最高统一。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing system, totality, ultimate ground, metaphysical aspiration, or overreach. (当分析系统、总体、终极根据、形而上学欲求或越界时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
`Idea of Reason (理性理念; de: Idee der Vernunft)`  
**Definition:** a concept of totality or the unconditioned that guides inquiry but cannot be given as an object in experience. (一种关于总体或无条件者的概念，它引导探究，但不能作为经验对象被给予。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains the regulative function of concepts such as soul, world, and God. (它解释灵魂、世界和上帝等概念的调节性功能。)  
**Why needed:** reason naturally seeks completeness, but possible experience never gives totality as an object. (理性自然寻求完整性，但可能经验从不给出作为对象的总体。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing metaphysical concepts that guide inquiry without being empirically knowable objects. (当分析那些引导探究但并非经验可知对象的形而上学概念时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Kant does not simply discard metaphysical ideas. He restricts their use. Ideas such as the soul, the world as totality, and God may have regulative significance. They guide inquiry toward unity. But when reason treats them as objects of theoretical knowledge, it falls into illusion.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Ideas of reason regulate inquiry, but they do not constitute objects of possible experience. (理性理念调节探究，但不构成可能经验的对象。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Constitutive Use (构成性使用; de: konstitutiver Gebrauch)** produces or structures objects of experience; **Regulative Use (调节性使用; de: regulativer Gebrauch)** guides inquiry without producing an object. (构成性使用产生或结构化经验对象；调节性使用引导探究，但不产生对象。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** Kant preserves metaphysical aspiration while denying dogmatic metaphysical knowledge. This tension defines much of post-Kantian philosophy. (康德保存形而上学欲求，同时否认独断的形而上学知识。这一张力塑造了大量后康德哲学。)  
  
### 17. Antinomy: The Problem of Reason against Itself  
  
`Antinomy (二律背反; el: ἀντινομία; de: Antinomie)`  
**Definition:** a conflict in which reason seems able to prove both a thesis and its opposite when it exceeds possible experience. (当理性越出可能经验时，它似乎既能证明一个命题，又能证明其反命题的冲突。)  
**Problem solved:** it diagnoses the self-conflict of reason in speculative metaphysics. (它诊断思辨形而上学中理性同自身的冲突。)  
**Why needed:** reason’s failure is not accidental; it arises from its natural drive toward the unconditioned. (理性的失败不是偶然的；它来自理性趋向无条件者的自然冲动。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing philosophical deadlocks generated by illegitimate metaphysical extension. (当分析由不合法的形而上学扩展所产生的哲学僵局时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Antinomy is Kant’s critical version of aporia. It shows that reason can trap itself when it tries to know totality as if it were an object. For example, reason may argue that the world must have a beginning in time, and also that it cannot have a beginning in time. The conflict arises because the world as totality is not an object of possible experience.  
  
This is not merely a logical puzzle. It is a warning system. When reason generates equally compelling opposed claims, the problem may lie not in insufficient data but in the misuse of concepts beyond experience.  
  
**Typical sentence:** An antinomy shows reason exceeding its legitimate field and producing conflict from its own demand for totality. (二律背反显示理性越出其合法领域，并从自身对总体性的要求中产生冲突。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** later philosophy often treats antinomy, contradiction, and aporia as productive rather than merely pathological. Hegel will transform contradiction into dialectical movement. Derrida will use aporia to expose limits within conceptual systems. **Aporia (难题; el: ἀπορία; fr: aporie)** becomes a name for a conceptual impasse that cannot be resolved within the existing conceptual scheme.  
  
### 18. Judgment: The Problem of Applying Concepts  
  
`Judgment (判断; de: Urteil)`  
**Definition:** the act through which a concept is applied, connected, or predicated in relation to intuition or another concept. (概念在同直观或另一概念的关系中被应用、连接或谓述的活动。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains how cognition moves from concepts and intuitions to determinate claims. (它解释认知如何从概念与直观走向确定主张。)  
**Why needed:** knowledge requires not only concepts and intuitions, but the capacity to connect them correctly. (知识不仅需要概念和直观，还需要正确连接二者的能力。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing application, predication, subsumption, or validity. (当分析应用、谓述、归摄或有效性时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Judgment is where Kantian cognition becomes operative. It is not enough to have intuitions and concepts separately. The mind must judge that this intuition falls under this concept, that this event follows according to a causal rule, that this manifold counts as one object.  
  
This is why judgment becomes a bridge between logic, epistemology, and aesthetics. It concerns the application of rules, but also the problem of cases where no determinate rule is immediately available.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Judgment is the power of bringing the particular under the universal. (判断是把个别者归入普遍者之下的能力。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** judgment becomes a major tool for later philosophy of law, aesthetics, political theory, and hermeneutics, because these fields often concern how general norms apply to particular cases. (判断成为后来法哲学、美学、政治理论和解释学的重要工具，因为这些领域经常关涉一般规范如何应用于特殊案例。)  
  
### 19. Autonomy: The Problem of Self-Legislation  
  
`Autonomy (自主性; el: αὐτονομία; de: Autonomie)`  
**Definition:** the capacity of reason or will to give law to itself. (理性或意志为自身立法的能力。)  
**Problem solved:** it grounds freedom not in arbitrary choice, but in rational self-legislation. (它把自由奠基于理性自我立法，而不是任意选择。)  
**Why needed:** morality requires a source of obligation that is neither mere external command nor private inclination. (道德需要一种义务来源，它既不是单纯外部命令，也不是私人倾向。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing moral law, freedom, responsibility, dignity, or rational agency. (当分析道德法则、自由、责任、尊严或理性行动者性时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Although this chapter focuses on theoretical philosophy, Kant’s critical vocabulary also transforms practical philosophy. The same basic move appears: do not ask only what actions are commanded; ask what makes obligation legitimate. Moral law must not depend merely on external authority, social custom, or empirical desire. It must be grounded in reason’s capacity to legislate universally.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Autonomy is not doing whatever one wants; it is acting according to a law reason can give to itself. (自主性不是想做什么就做什么，而是按照理性能够为自身给出的法则行动。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Autonomy (自主性; de: Autonomie)** contrasts with **Heteronomy (他律; de: Heteronomie)**. Autonomy means self-legislation by reason; heteronomy means determination by something external to rational self-legislation. (自主性是理性的自我立法；他律是由理性自我立法之外的东西来规定。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** autonomy becomes one of the central modern terms for morality, law, politics, personhood, and rights. Later thinkers will question whether the autonomous subject is universal, embodied, gendered, social, historical, or disciplined. (自主性成为现代道德、法律、政治、人格和权利的核心术语之一。后来的思想家会追问自主主体是否是普遍的、具身的、性别化的、社会的、历史的或被规训的。)  
  
### 20. The Tool-Map of Kantian Critique  
  
Use Kantian vocabulary diagnostically. The question is usually not “What is the object?” but “What makes objectivity possible?”  
  
**If the text asks what makes experience possible**, look for **Transcendental (先验的; de: transzendental)** and **Condition of Possibility (可能性条件; de: Bedingung der Möglichkeit)**.  
(如果文本追问经验何以可能，应寻找先验与可能性条件问题。)  
  
**If the text distinguishes empirical knowledge from non-empirical necessity**, look for **A priori (先天的; la: a priori)** and **A posteriori (后天的; la: a posteriori)**.  
(如果文本区分经验知识与非经验必然性，应寻找先天与后天问题。)  
  
**If the text asks how objects are given**, look for **Intuition (直观; de: Anschauung)**, **Sensibility (感性; de: Sinnlichkeit)**, **Space (空间; de: Raum)**, and **Time (时间; de: Zeit)**.  
(如果文本追问对象如何被给予，应寻找直观、感性、空间与时间问题。)  
  
**If the text asks how objects are thought**, look for **Concept (概念; de: Begriff)**, **Understanding (知性; de: Verstand)**, and **Category (范畴; de: Kategorie)**.  
(如果文本追问对象如何被思考，应寻找概念、知性与范畴问题。)  
  
**If the text asks how multiplicity becomes unity**, look for **Synthesis (综合; de: Synthesis)**, **Imagination (想象力; de: Einbildungskraft)**, and **Apperception (统觉; de: Apperzeption)**.  
(如果文本追问复多如何成为统一，应寻找综合、想象力与统觉问题。)  
  
**If the text asks where knowledge stops**, look for **Phenomenon (现象; de: Erscheinung)**, **Noumenon (智思物/本体; de: Noumenon)**, **Thing-in-itself (物自身; de: Ding an sich)**, and **Limit (限度; de: Grenze)**.  
(如果文本追问知识在哪里停止，应寻找现象、物自身与限度问题。)  
  
**If the text asks why reason produces metaphysical conflict**, look for **Reason (理性; de: Vernunft)**, **Idea of Reason (理性理念; de: Idee der Vernunft)**, and **Antinomy (二律背反; de: Antinomie)**.  
(如果文本追问理性为何产生形而上学冲突，应寻找理性、理性理念与二律背反问题。)  
  
**If the text asks how moral obligation is possible**, look for **Autonomy (自主性; de: Autonomie)**, **Moral Law (道德法则; de: moralisches Gesetz)**, and **Heteronomy (他律; de: Heteronomie)**.  
(如果文本追问道德义务何以可能，应寻找自主性、道德法则与他律问题。)  
  
### 21. The Genealogical Point of Part 4  
  
Kantian critique transforms the philosophical problem of knowledge. Greek philosophy asked how being, truth, nature, and form are intelligible. Latin metaphysics asked how finite beings are ordered through substance, essence, existence, law, and cause. Early modern philosophy asked how a subject can secure access to an object through representation and method. Kant asks a deeper structural question: **what conditions make objects, experience, and knowledge possible in the first place?** (康德追问更深层的结构问题：对象、经验与知识首先凭什么条件成为可能？)  
  
The guiding thesis is:  
  
**Kantian philosophical language turns knowledge into a problem of conditions: to know is not merely to represent an object, but to experience an object under forms, concepts, categories, synthesis, and the unity of consciousness.**  
(康德哲学语言把知识转化为条件问题：认识不只是表象对象，而是在形式、概念、范畴、综合与意识统一性之下经验对象。)  
  
This grammar remains decisive for later philosophy. German Idealism will ask whether the subject’s synthetic activity can be understood historically and absolutely. Phenomenology will transform transcendental inquiry into an analysis of intentional consciousness. Analytic philosophy will inherit the concern for conditions, validity, judgment, and objectivity in a different register. Foucault will historicize the Kantian question by asking under what historical conditions something can count as knowledge. Derrida will radicalize the problem of conditions by showing that conditions of possibility may also be conditions of instability.  
  
The Kantian question therefore becomes one of the major engines of modern thought:  
  
**What must be presupposed for something to appear, count, or be known as something?**  
(为了使某物能够作为某物而显现、被承认或被认识，必须预设什么？)  
  
## Part 5. German Idealism: Spirit, Negation, Dialectic  
  
This chapter explains how German Idealism transforms Kantian critique into a philosophy of activity, history, and self-development. Kant had asked what conditions make experience and knowledge possible. German Idealism asks whether those conditions can themselves be understood as dynamic, self-generating, social, and historical.  
  
The key vocabulary changes accordingly. The central terms are **I**, **Self-Consciousness**, **Spirit**, **Concept**, **Recognition**, **Negation**, **Mediation**, **Contradiction**, **Dialectic**, **Aufhebung**, **Alienation**, and **Actuality**. **Aufhebung (扬弃; de: Aufhebung)** is a central Hegelian term meaning cancellation, preservation, and elevation in one movement; dialectic is a movement driven by contradiction and sublation.  
  
The operational function of this chapter is clear: use German Idealist vocabulary when the problem is not merely **what the conditions of knowledge are**, but **how those conditions develop through activity, opposition, and historical mediation**. (当问题不只是“知识条件是什么”，而是“这些条件如何通过活动、对立与历史中介而发展”时，应使用德国观念论词汇。)  
  
### 1. The Problem-Situation: From Conditions to Development  
  
Kant’s critical philosophy established limits. Human knowledge is conditioned by sensibility, understanding, categories, synthesis, and apperception. But this leaves a pressure unresolved: are these conditions fixed structures, or do they develop? Are subject and object permanently divided, or can their opposition be overcome? Is reason merely a faculty inside the human mind, or does reason unfold historically in institutions, culture, and social life?  
  
German Idealism emerges from these pressures.  
  
The central question becomes:  
  
**How can subject and object, thought and being, freedom and necessity, individual and world be understood as moments of one developing rational process?**  
(主体与客体、思想与存在、自由与必然、个体与世界，如何能够被理解为同一个发展中的理性过程的诸环节？)  
  
This question changes philosophical grammar. Philosophy no longer treats concepts as static definitions. A concept must be understood through its movement, its negations, its failures, and its development into a richer form.  
  
This is why German Idealism needs **Dialectic (辩证法; de: Dialektik)**. It is not merely a debate technique. It is a logic of development. A position reveals its own limitation, passes into its opposite, and is transformed into a more complex unity.  
  
**Typical sentence:** A concept is not fully understood by definition alone; it must be followed through the movement by which it overcomes its own one-sidedness. (一个概念不能只通过定义得到充分理解；必须追踪它克服自身片面性的运动。)  
  
### 2. Idealism: The Problem of the Activity of Thought  
  
`Idealism (观念论; de: Idealismus)`  
**Definition:** the view that objectivity is inseparable from the activity, structure, or self-development of thought. (一种认为客观性不能脱离思想的活动、结构或自我发展的观点。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains why objects are not merely given to a passive mind but are constituted, organized, or mediated by thought. (它解释为什么对象并非只是被给予一个被动心灵，而是由思想构成、组织或中介。)  
**Why needed:** Kant had shown that objectivity depends on conditions of cognition; German Idealism asks whether these conditions belong to a larger activity of reason. (康德已经显示客观性依赖认知条件；德国观念论追问这些条件是否属于理性的更大活动。)  
**How to use:** use it when the issue is the role of thought, subjectivity, or reason in making objectivity intelligible. (当问题涉及思想、主体性或理性在使客观性成为可理解之物中的作用时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
German Idealism should not be reduced to the claim that “everything is in the mind.” That is too crude. Its central concern is the intelligibility of objectivity. If an object is an object only within conditions of cognition, then philosophy must explain the activity through which objectivity is formed.  
  
This does not simply deny the world. It asks how the world becomes intelligible as world. The object is no longer treated as wholly external to thought; it is understood through relation, mediation, and concept.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Idealism does not simply erase the object; it asks how the object becomes intelligible within the activity of thought. (观念论并不简单取消对象；它追问对象如何在思想活动中成为可理解之物。)
