**Conceptual contrast:** **Idealism (观念论; de: Idealismus)** contrasts with **Naive Realism (朴素实在论; de: naiver Realismus)**. Naive realism treats objects as simply given independently of cognition; idealism asks how objectivity is mediated by thought. (朴素实在论把对象视为简单地独立于认知而给定；观念论追问客观性如何由思想中介。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** Kant’s transcendental conditions become, in post-Kantian idealism, a problem of self-positing activity, historical development, and rational totality. (康德的先验条件在后康德观念论中转化为自我设定活动、历史发展与理性总体的问题。)  
  
### 3. The I: The Problem of Self-Positing Activity  
  
`I (自我; de: Ich)`  
**Definition:** the self-relating subject that posits, acts, and organizes experience. (自我关联、设定、行动并组织经验的主体。)  
**Problem solved:** it gives philosophy a principle of activity rather than mere reception. (它为哲学提供一个活动原则，而不只是接受性原则。)  
**Why needed:** if knowledge and freedom require activity, the subject must be understood as more than a passive site of representations. (如果知识与自由需要活动，主体就必须被理解为不只是表象的被动场所。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing self-activity, self-relation, agency, or the grounding function of subjectivity. (当分析自我活动、自我关系、行动者性或主体性的奠基功能时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
The German Idealist **I** radicalizes the early modern subject and the Kantian unity of apperception. In Fichte, the **I** is not merely discovered; it posits itself. This means that subjectivity is not a thing behind experience but an activity that institutes a field of experience and action.  
  
This is a crucial tool. It shifts philosophy from substance to act. The self is not primarily a static entity. It is a doing.  
  
**Typical sentence:** The I is not first a thing that has activity; it is self-relating activity itself. (自我首先不是拥有活动的东西，而是自我关联的活动本身。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **I (自我; de: Ich)** contrasts with **Not-I (非我; de: Nicht-Ich)**. The I posits itself, but it also encounters limitation, resistance, or opposition in the Not-I. (自我设定自身，但也在非我中遭遇限制、阻力或对立。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** the **I** becomes a dynamic principle rather than an epistemic point of certainty. Descartes’ **Cogito (我思; la: cogito)** secures self-certainty; German Idealism asks how selfhood is actively produced and limited. (自我成为一种动态原则，而不只是认识论确定性点。笛卡尔的我思确保自我确定性；德国观念论追问自我性如何被主动生产并受到限制。)  
  
### 4. Not-I and Limitation: The Problem of Resistance  
  
`Not-I (非我; de: Nicht-Ich)`  
**Definition:** that which limits, resists, or stands opposed to the self-positing I. (限制、抵抗或对立于自我设定之自我的东西。)  
**Problem solved:** it prevents the I from collapsing into empty self-enclosure. (它防止自我坍缩为空洞的自我封闭。)  
**Why needed:** activity becomes determinate only through limitation. (活动只有通过限制才变得确定。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing opposition, resistance, objectivity, or the boundary of subjectivity. (当分析对立、阻力、客观性或主体性的边界时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
The **Not-I** solves a problem internal to idealism. If the I is pure activity, why is experience not arbitrary? Why does the subject encounter resistance? Why is there something rather than mere self-display?  
  
The Not-I introduces limitation. It gives the I something against which to act, strive, and determine itself. This means objectivity is not simply outside the subject; it is the form of resistance through which subjectivity becomes determinate.  
  
**Typical sentence:** The I becomes determinate only by encountering what limits it. (自我只有通过遭遇限制它的东西才成为确定者。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Limitation (限制; de: Grenze/Beschränkung)** is not simple negation. It is the condition through which finite activity becomes determinate. (限制不是简单否定，而是有限活动成为确定者的条件。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** this structure prepares later dialectical thought: identity is not self-enclosed but constituted through opposition. (这一结构为后来的辩证思想做准备：同一性不是自我封闭的，而是通过对立而构成的。)  
  
### 5. Absolute: The Problem of the Whole  
  
`Absolute (绝对者; de: das Absolute)`  
**Definition:** that which is not dependent on an external condition; the whole within which oppositions are grounded or reconciled. (不依赖外部条件者；对立在其中得到奠基或和解的整体。)  
**Problem solved:** it answers the demand for an ultimate unity beyond finite oppositions. (它回应超出有限对立的最终统一性要求。)  
**Why needed:** if philosophy remains within subject/object, freedom/nature, and thought/being oppositions, it cannot achieve systematic completeness. (如果哲学停留在主体/客体、自由/自然、思想/存在的对立中，就无法达到系统完整性。)  
**How to use:** use it when the issue is totality, ultimate ground, or the reconciliation of fundamental oppositions. (当问题涉及总体性、终极根据或根本对立的和解时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
The **Absolute** is not simply a very large object. It is the demand that philosophy not stop at divided terms. Kant had placed limits on knowledge and preserved distinctions between phenomenon and noumenon, understanding and reason, nature and freedom. German Idealism asks whether these divisions can be overcome within a higher unity.  
  
This creates a systematic ambition: philosophy must not merely analyze fragments; it must think the whole.  
  
**Typical sentence:** The Absolute is not one object within the system; it is the unity in terms of which the system becomes intelligible. (绝对者不是系统内部的一个对象，而是系统凭之成为可理解整体的统一性。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Absolute (绝对者; de: das Absolute)** contrasts with **Finite (有限者; de: das Endliche)**. The finite depends on conditions and limits; the absolute is thought as that within which such conditions and limits are grounded. (有限者依赖条件和限制；绝对者被思为这些条件与限制得以奠基的整体。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** the post-Kantian search for the Absolute becomes both the peak and the target of later critique. Kierkegaard, Marx, Nietzsche, Heidegger, and post-structuralist thinkers will all challenge forms of totalizing reason. (后康德思想对绝对者的追求既成为高峰，也成为后来批判的靶子。)  
  
### 6. Spirit: The Problem of Reason as Historical Life  
  
`Spirit (精神; de: Geist)`  
**Definition:** reason understood not merely as an individual faculty but as social, historical, cultural, and institutional life. (理性不再只是个体能力，而是社会的、历史的、文化的和制度性的生命。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains how reason exists in practices, institutions, language, art, religion, and history. (它解释理性如何存在于实践、制度、语言、艺术、宗教与历史之中。)  
**Why needed:** individual consciousness alone cannot explain the historical and social forms through which meaning and freedom become actual. (单一个体意识无法解释意义与自由得以现实化的历史和社会形式。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing reason as embodied in collective forms rather than isolated mental acts. (当把理性分析为体现于集体形式，而非孤立心灵活动时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
**Geist** should not be flattened into “mind.” It can mean spirit, mind, culture, collective rational life, or historically embodied meaning. Its power lies in this breadth. It allows Hegel to think reason beyond the private subject.  
  
This is one of the decisive moves of German Idealism. The subject is not merely an individual consciousness standing before an object. The subject belongs to social and historical forms. Language, law, family, civil society, state, religion, art, and philosophy are not external decorations of thought. They are forms in which spirit becomes actual.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Spirit is reason become historical, social, and institutional. (精神是成为历史的、社会的和制度性的理性。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Spirit (精神; de: Geist)** differs from **Consciousness (意识; de: Bewusstsein)**. Consciousness can name the relation of a subject to an object; spirit names the broader historical life in which subjectivity and objectivity are mediated. (意识可以命名主体与客体的关系；精神则命名主体性与客观性在其中被中介的更广阔历史生命。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** Geist transforms the modern subject into a historical form of life. Later Marx will materialize and criticize this structure through labor, class, and ideology. (精神把现代主体转化为历史性的生活形式。后来马克思会通过劳动、阶级和意识形态使这一结构物质化并加以批判。)  
  
### 7. Concept: The Problem of Living Structure  
  
`Concept (概念; de: Begriff)`  
**Definition:** not merely a general representation, but a self-developing rational structure that determines and unfolds itself. (不仅是一般表象，而是自我发展、自我规定并展开自身的理性结构。)  
**Problem solved:** it makes concepts dynamic rather than static labels. (它使概念成为动态结构，而不是静态标签。)  
**Why needed:** if reality is rationally structured and historically developing, concepts must be able to express movement and development. (如果现实具有理性结构并在历史中发展，概念就必须能够表达运动与发展。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing a term not as a definition but as a process of self-determination. (当把一个术语分析为自我规定过程，而非单纯定义时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
In Kant, **Concept (概念; de: Begriff)** is a general representation that helps organize intuition. In Hegel, **Begriff** becomes much stronger. It is the inner structure by which something develops into its truth. A concept is not complete at its first abstract formulation. It must pass through its determinations.  
  
This gives Hegelian language its distinctive difficulty. A word such as freedom, being, essence, right, or spirit does not mean only one fixed thing. It means differently at different stages of its development. The task is to follow the concept.  
  
**Typical sentence:** The truth of a concept lies not in its first abstraction but in the movement through which it becomes concrete. (一个概念的真理不在其最初抽象中，而在它成为具体者的运动中。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Abstract Concept (抽象概念; de: abstrakter Begriff)** gives a one-sided determination; **Concrete Concept (具体概念; de: konkreter Begriff)** contains mediated difference within unity. (抽象概念给出片面的规定；具体概念则在统一中包含被中介的差异。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** the concept becomes historical and developmental. This prepares later forms of social theory, ideology critique, and genealogy, all of which treat concepts as historically formed rather than timeless labels. (概念成为历史性的、发展性的。这为后来的社会理论、意识形态批判和谱系学做准备，它们都把概念视为历史形成之物，而非永恒标签。)  
  
### 8. Self-Consciousness: The Problem of Selfhood through Otherness  
  
`Self-Consciousness (自我意识; de: Selbstbewusstsein)`  
**Definition:** consciousness that relates to itself as itself. (以自身为自身而与自身发生关系的意识。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains how a subject is not merely aware of objects but aware of itself in relation to objects and others. (它解释主体如何不只是意识到对象，而且在同对象和他者的关系中意识到自身。)  
**Why needed:** subjectivity requires self-relation, not merely perception. (主体性需要自我关系，而不只是知觉。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing reflexivity, desire, recognition, struggle, or the social formation of selfhood. (当分析反身性、欲望、承认、斗争或自我的社会形成时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
German Idealism transforms self-consciousness from inner certainty into relational development. The self does not fully know itself by looking inward. It becomes self-conscious through relation to what is other: object, world, another self-consciousness, institution, and history.  
  
This is the key to Hegel’s famous movement from consciousness to self-consciousness. Consciousness first confronts objects. Self-consciousness discovers that it needs recognition from another self-consciousness. The self is not complete in isolation.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Self-consciousness becomes actual only through relation to what is other than itself. (自我意识只有通过同异于自身者的关系才成为现实。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Consciousness (意识; de: Bewusstsein)** relates to an object; **Self-Consciousness (自我意识; de: Selbstbewusstsein)** relates to itself through that relation. (意识与对象发生关系；自我意识则通过这种关系同自身发生关系。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** selfhood becomes social and conflictual. Later theories of recognition, alienation, ideology, intersubjectivity, psychoanalysis, and social construction all inherit this move. (自我性变成社会性的、冲突性的。后来的承认理论、异化理论、意识形态理论、主体间性、精神分析和社会建构论都继承了这一转变。)  
  
### 9. Recognition: The Problem of Social Selfhood  
  
`Recognition (承认; de: Anerkennung)`  
**Definition:** the social relation through which a self is acknowledged as a self by another self. (一个自我被另一个自我承认为自我的社会关系。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains why selfhood and freedom require social validation rather than private certainty alone. (它解释为什么自我性与自由需要社会承认，而不只是私人确定性。)  
**Why needed:** a subject cannot be fully actual as free unless its freedom is recognized by others and embodied in institutions. (除非主体的自由被他者承认并体现在制度中，否则主体不能作为自由者充分现实化。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing social identity, struggle, dignity, rights, authority, or mutuality. (当分析社会身份、斗争、尊严、权利、权威或相互性时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
**Usage layers:**  
1. **Hegelian use (黑格尔式用法):** **recognition (Anerkennung)** names the process through which self-consciousness becomes itself through being recognized by another self-consciousness. (在黑格尔那里，承认指自我意识通过被另一个自我意识承认而成为自身的过程。)  
  
2. **Critical-theory reception use (批判理论接受史用法):** in later social and political theory, recognition becomes a vocabulary for dignity, social freedom, intersubjective validation, respect, and institutional membership. (在后来的社会政治理论中，承认成为尊严、社会自由、主体间确认、尊重和制度成员身份的词汇。)  
  
3. **Contemporary transferable use (当代理论泛用法):** in feminism, queer theory, race theory, disability studies, and postcolonial theory, recognition often concerns who becomes socially intelligible, credible, visible, and normatively protected. (在女性主义、酷儿理论、种族理论、残障研究和后殖民理论中，承认常关涉谁能成为社会上可理解、可信、可见并受规范保护的主体。)  
  
**Transfer rule:** use **recognition** when identity, agency, or freedom depends on social acknowledgment. Do not use it merely for psychological approval or polite acceptance. (转用规则：当身份、行动能力或自由依赖社会承认时，才使用 recognition。不要把它仅仅当成心理认可或礼貌接受。)  
  
**Misuse warning:** recognition can liberate, but it can also normalize. Ask what form of recognition is being granted and under what conditions. (承认可以解放，也可以正常化。应追问被授予的是什么形式的承认，以及条件是什么。)  
  
Recognition is one of the most powerful tools in modern philosophy. It shifts the problem of subjectivity from inward certainty to social relation. The subject becomes itself through being recognized by another subject.  
  
This also means that conflict is not accidental. Recognition can fail. It can be unequal, denied, coerced, or distorted. The struggle for recognition becomes a structure of social and political life.  
  
**Typical sentence:** A self becomes socially real only when its freedom is recognized by another. (一个自我只有在其自由被他者承认时才具有社会现实性。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Recognition (承认; de: Anerkennung)** differs from **Mere Acknowledgment (单纯承认/承认事实; en: acknowledgment)**. Recognition is not just noticing that someone exists; it grants or confirms status. (承认不是仅仅注意到某人存在，而是赋予或确认其地位。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** recognition becomes central for later theories of rights, identity, labor, gender, race, coloniality, and social justice. The Greek question of justice and the Latin question of personhood are now reworked through mutual social validation. (承认成为后来权利、身份、劳动、性别、种族、殖民性和社会正义理论的核心。希腊的正义问题与拉丁的人格问题在这里被改写为相互社会确认的问题。)  
  
### 10. Negation: The Problem of Productive Opposition  
  
`Negation (否定; de: Negation)`  
**Definition:** the act or structure by which a determination is denied, limited, opposed, or transformed. (一个规定被否认、限制、对立或转化的活动或结构。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains how development can occur through opposition rather than simple accumulation. (它解释发展如何能够通过对立发生，而不只是通过简单累积发生。)  
**Why needed:** concepts and forms of life reveal their limits through what they exclude or fail to contain. (概念和生活形式通过其排除或无法包含之物显现其限度。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing contradiction, opposition, failure, transformation, or critical movement. (当分析矛盾、对立、失败、转化或批判运动时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Negation is not merely saying “no.” In German Idealism, negation is productive. A concept becomes determinate by excluding what it is not. But this exclusion also creates instability. What is excluded can return as a problem.  
  
For Hegel, development occurs because a form reveals its own insufficiency. It negates itself by failing to be what it claims to be. This is why negation drives movement.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Negation is not external destruction; it is the movement through which a form reveals and transforms its own limit. (否定不是外部破坏，而是一个形式揭示并转化自身限度的运动。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Abstract Negation (抽象否定; de: abstrakte Negation)** simply cancels; **Determinate Negation (规定性否定; de: bestimmte Negation)** produces a new determination. (抽象否定只是取消；规定性否定产生新的规定。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** productive negation becomes a model for critique. Marx will use contradiction to analyze capitalism. Psychoanalysis will analyze repression and return. Derrida will show how excluded terms destabilize conceptual hierarchies. (生产性否定成为批判的模型。马克思会用矛盾分析资本主义。精神分析会分析压抑与回返。德里达会显示被排除项如何动摇概念等级。)  
  
### 11. Contradiction: The Problem of Internal Instability  
  
`Contradiction (矛盾; de: Widerspruch)`  
**Definition:** an internal opposition in which a form, concept, or institution conflicts with itself. (一个形式、概念或制度同自身发生冲突的内部对立。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains why development is necessary rather than optional. (它解释为什么发展是必要的，而不是可有可无的。)  
**Why needed:** a form changes not only because something external attacks it, but because its own structure becomes unstable. (一个形式发生变化，不只是因为外部事物攻击它，也因为其自身结构变得不稳定。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing internal tension, self-undermining claims, social conflict, or conceptual breakdown. (当分析内部张力、自我破坏的主张、社会冲突或概念崩溃时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
In formal logic, contradiction is usually a defect. In Hegelian dialectic, contradiction is also a motor. This does not mean that contradictions are simply acceptable. It means that contradictions reveal where a concept or institution cannot remain as it is.  
  
For example, a social order may claim universal freedom while depending on domination. That contradiction is not merely a logical error. It is a historical force. It presses the order toward transformation.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Contradiction is the internal pressure by which a form is forced beyond its own immediacy. (矛盾是一个形式被迫超出其自身直接性的内部压力。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **External Opposition (外部对立; de: äußerer Gegensatz)** occurs between separate terms; **Internal Contradiction (内部矛盾; de: innerer Widerspruch)** belongs to the structure of the thing itself. (外部对立发生在分离项之间；内部矛盾属于事物自身结构。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** contradiction becomes central for Marxist critique, critical theory, and many forms of social analysis. A society is not criticized only by external moral standards; it may be criticized by showing that it fails by its own norms. (矛盾成为马克思主义批判、批判理论和多种社会分析的核心。批判一个社会不只是诉诸外部道德标准，也可以显示它按自身规范而失败。)  
  
### 12. Mediation: The Problem of Non-Immediacy  
  
`Mediation (中介; de: Vermittlung)`  
**Definition:** the process through which something becomes what it is by passing through relations, oppositions, or otherness. (某物通过关系、对立或他异性而成为其所是的过程。)  
**Problem solved:** it prevents philosophy from treating identity, knowledge, or freedom as immediately given. (它防止哲学把同一性、知识或自由视为直接给定。)  
**Why needed:** complex realities are produced through relations, not isolated self-presence. (复杂现实是通过关系产生的，而不是通过孤立的自我在场产生的。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing how a thing depends on what seems external to it. (当分析某物如何依赖看似外在于它的东西时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Mediation is one of the most important German Idealist tools. It allows philosophy to reject immediate certainty. A thing is not simply what it first appears to be. It becomes intelligible only through the relations that form it.  
  
The self is mediated by the other. Freedom is mediated by institutions. Knowledge is mediated by concepts. Spirit is mediated by history. Even immediacy is usually mediated immediacy: something appears immediate only because its mediating conditions have been forgotten.  
  
**Typical sentence:** What appears immediate is often the result of forgotten mediation. (看似直接的东西，往往是被遗忘的中介的结果。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Immediacy (直接性; de: Unmittelbarkeit)** claims direct givenness; **Mediation (中介; de: Vermittlung)** reveals the relational process that makes such givenness possible. (直接性声称直接给予；中介揭示使这种给予成为可能的关系过程。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** mediation becomes indispensable for social theory, hermeneutics, ideology critique, and genealogy. Genealogy later radicalizes this point by asking what historical mediations have been hidden under claims of nature, truth, or immediacy. (中介对社会理论、解释学、意识形态批判和谱系学都不可或缺。谱系学后来激进化这一点，追问哪些历史中介被“自然”“真理”或“直接性”的名义遮蔽了。)  
  
### 13. Dialectic: The Problem of Development through Opposition  
  
`Dialectic (辩证法; el: διαλεκτική; de: Dialektik)`  
**Definition:** the movement through which a concept or form develops by encountering its own negation and being transformed into a richer unity. (概念或形式通过遭遇自身否定并被转化为更丰富统一性的运动。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains conceptual and historical development without reducing it to linear accumulation. (它解释概念和历史发展，而不把发展化约为线性累积。)  
**Why needed:** thought and history move through tensions, failures, reversals, and transformations. (思想与历史通过张力、失败、反转和转化而运动。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing a sequence in which a position becomes unstable, passes into opposition, and is transformed. (当分析一个立场变得不稳定、进入对立并被转化的过程时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Dialectic is often simplified as thesis-antithesis-synthesis. That formula can be pedagogically useful, but it is too mechanical. Hegelian dialectic is not a three-step template imposed from outside. It is the immanent movement of a form that discovers its own insufficiency.  
  
Dialectic is therefore a reading method. When reading a dialectical text, do not ask only what the author asserts. Ask: what limitation does this assertion generate? What does it exclude? How does that exclusion return? What richer form becomes necessary?  
  
**Typical sentence:** Dialectic follows the immanent movement by which a form becomes other than itself in order to become more fully itself. (辩证法追踪一个形式的内在运动：它成为异于自身者，以便更充分地成为自身。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Dialectic (辩证法; de: Dialektik)** differs from **External Refutation (外在反驳; en: external refutation)**. External refutation attacks a claim from outside; dialectic shows how the claim undermines itself from within. (外在反驳从外部攻击一个主张；辩证法显示该主张如何从内部瓦解自身。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** dialectic becomes one of the main languages of modern critique. Marx materializes it; Kierkegaard existentializes it; Adorno radicalizes its negativity; post-structuralism often rejects totalizing dialectic while preserving attention to instability and opposition. (辩证法成为现代批判的主要语言之一。马克思使其物质化；克尔凯郭尔使其存在论化；阿多诺激进化其否定性；后结构主义常拒绝总体化辩证法，但保留对不稳定性和对立的关注。)  
  
### 14. Aufhebung: The Problem of Transformation without Simple Loss  
  
`Aufhebung (扬弃; de: Aufhebung)`  
**Definition:** cancellation, preservation, and elevation in one dialectical movement. (在同一辩证运动中取消、保存并提升。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains how a stage can be overcome without being simply erased. (它解释一个阶段如何能够被克服而不是被简单抹除。)  
**Why needed:** historical and conceptual development require continuity through transformation. (历史与概念发展需要在转化中保持连续性。)  
**How to use:** use it when a concept, institution, or form is negated yet retained in a higher or more complex form. (当一个概念、制度或形式被否定但又在更高或更复杂形式中被保留时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
**Aufhebung** is difficult because it contains opposed meanings. It means to cancel, to preserve, and to lift up. This is not an accident. It is the structure of dialectical transformation. A lower form is not simply destroyed. It is preserved as a moment within a higher form.  
  
For example, immediate certainty may be aufgehoben in mediated knowledge. It is canceled as naive immediacy, preserved as a moment of experience, and elevated into a more reflective form. A social form may be aufgehoben when its partial freedom is negated, preserved, and transformed into a more universal freedom.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Aufhebung names a negation that preserves what it overcomes by transforming its place in the whole. (扬弃命名一种否定：它通过改变被克服者在整体中的位置而保存它。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Destruction (摧毁; de: Zerstörung)** simply eliminates; **Aufhebung (扬弃; de: Aufhebung)** transforms by canceling and preserving at once. (摧毁只是消除；扬弃则同时取消并保存，从而完成转化。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** the concept of Aufhebung shapes later theories of historical development, revolution, critique, and institutional transformation. It also becomes a target for anti-dialectical thinkers who reject the idea that loss can be reconciled within a higher unity. (扬弃塑造后来的历史发展、革命、批判和制度转化理论；它也成为反辩证思想的靶子，因为后者拒绝认为损失可以在更高统一中被和解。)  
  
### 15. Alienation: The Problem of Spirit Estranged from Itself  
  
`Alienation (异化; de: Entfremdung/Entäußerung)`  
**Definition:** the condition in which a subject, spirit, or activity becomes estranged from itself in an external form. (主体、精神或活动在外部形式中同自身相疏离的状态。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains how self-expression can become self-loss. (它解释自我表达如何可能变成自我丧失。)  
**Why needed:** historical development often requires externalization, but externalization can turn against its source. (历史发展常需要外化，但外化物可能反过来支配其来源。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing estrangement, loss of control, objectified activity, social domination, or misrecognition. (当分析疏离、失控、对象化活动、社会支配或错误承认时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Alienation is one of the bridges from Hegel to Marx. In Hegel, spirit externalizes itself in objects, institutions, and history. This externalization is not only negative; it is necessary for development. But when the externalized form is not recognized as one’s own, alienation occurs.  
  
Marx later materializes this structure. Labor produces objects and institutions that confront workers as alien powers. A spiritual-dialectical concept becomes a social-economic critique.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Alienation occurs when what a subject produces returns as something foreign and dominating. (当主体所生产之物反过来作为陌生且支配性的东西出现时，异化就发生了。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Externalization (外化; de: Entäußerung)** is the process by which spirit or activity becomes objective; **Alienation (异化; de: Entfremdung)** is externalization experienced as estrangement or domination. (外化是精神或活动成为客观者的过程；异化则是作为疏离或支配而被经验到的外化。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** alienation becomes central for Marxism, existentialism, psychoanalysis, critical theory, and sociology. It turns metaphysical estrangement into a tool for diagnosing modern social life. (异化成为马克思主义、存在主义、精神分析、批判理论和社会学的核心概念。它把形而上学疏离转化为诊断现代社会生活的工具。)  
  
### 16. Actuality: The Problem of Rational Realization  
  
`Actuality (现实性; de: Wirklichkeit)`  
**Definition:** not mere existence, but reality as effective, developed, and rationally articulated. (不是单纯存在，而是作为有效的、发展了的、理性地展开的现实。)  
**Problem solved:** it distinguishes what merely exists from what has become fully effective in a rational form. (它把单纯存在之物同已经在理性形式中充分有效化之物区分开来。)  
**Why needed:** philosophy needs a concept for realized rational structure, not just factual presence. (哲学需要一个概念来命名已经实现的理性结构，而不只是事实上的在场。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing whether a concept, freedom, institution, or form of life has become effective in the world. (当分析一个概念、自由、制度或生活形式是否已经在世界中成为有效现实时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
**Wirklichkeit** is often mistranslated if treated as mere “reality.” It carries the sense of effectiveness, actuality, and realized operation. Something may exist without being fully actual in Hegel’s strong sense. A right may be formally declared but not socially actual. Freedom may be abstractly affirmed but not institutionally realized.  
  
This makes actuality a critical tool. It asks whether a principle has become effective in practice.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Actuality is not bare existence; it is the effective realization of a rational form. (现实性不是赤裸存在，而是理性形式的有效实现。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Existence (存在/实存; de: Existenz)** may mean that something is there; **Actuality (现实性; de: Wirklichkeit)** means that it has achieved effective rational form. (存在可以指某物在那里；现实性则指某物已经达到有效的理性形式。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** actuality becomes a key tool for social and political critique. It allows philosophy to ask whether declared freedom, equality, law, or recognition is merely formal or actually realized. (现实性成为社会和政治批判的关键工具。它使哲学能够追问：被宣称的自由、平等、法律或承认只是形式上的，还是已经现实化？)  
  
### 17. Freedom: The Problem of Realized Self-Determination  
  
`Freedom (自由; de: Freiheit)`  
**Definition:** not mere arbitrary choice, but self-determination realized through rational and social forms. (不是单纯任意选择，而是通过理性与社会形式实现的自我规定。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains why freedom requires institutions, recognition, and actuality rather than private will alone. (它解释为什么自由需要制度、承认与现实性，而不只是私人意志。)  
**Why needed:** abstract freedom can remain empty unless it becomes embodied in social life. (抽象自由如果不体现于社会生活中，就可能保持空洞。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing autonomy, recognition, right, institution, ethical life, or historical emancipation. (当分析自主性、承认、权利、制度、伦理生活或历史解放时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
**Transfer rule:** before using **Freedom**, ask whether the problem is non-domination, moral autonomy, social recognition, material emancipation, existential responsibility, decolonization, bodily autonomy, or practical capacity under conditions. (转用规则：使用 Freedom 之前，应先判断问题是非支配、道德自主、社会承认、物质解放、存在主义责任、去殖民化、身体自主，还是处境中的实践能力。)  
  
German Idealist freedom develops Kantian autonomy. Kant grounds morality in rational self-legislation. Hegel argues that freedom must become actual in ethical and institutional life. Freedom is not simply the ability to choose among options. It is the condition in which the subject recognizes itself in the rational order of its world.  
  
This is why Hegel can treat family, civil society, law, and the state as philosophical topics. They are not external to freedom. They are possible forms of freedom’s realization.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Freedom becomes actual only when self-determination is embodied in institutions and mutual recognition. (自由只有在自我规定体现于制度和相互承认中时才成为现实。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Abstract Freedom (抽象自由; de: abstrakte Freiheit)** is mere indeterminate choice or negation; **Concrete Freedom (具体自由; de: konkrete Freiheit)** is freedom mediated by rational social forms. (抽象自由只是未规定的选择或否定；具体自由则是由理性社会形式中介的自由。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** this concept becomes crucial for Marx, liberalism, communitarianism, critical theory, and recognition theory. Later critique asks whether institutions realize freedom or disguise domination. (这一概念对马克思、自由主义、共同体主义、批判理论和承认理论都很关键。后来的批判会追问制度是在实现自由，还是在掩盖支配。)  
  
### 18. Ethical Life: The Problem of Freedom in Institutions  
  
`Ethical Life (伦理生活; de: Sittlichkeit)`  
**Definition:** the social and institutional life in which freedom, duty, and identity are concretely embodied. (自由、义务与身份在其中得到具体体现的社会与制度生活。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains how morality becomes more than private intention. (它解释道德如何超出私人意图。)  
**Why needed:** individual moral will requires social forms in which it can become actual. (个体道德意志需要社会形式，才能成为现实。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing family, civil society, state, institutions, custom, law, or social freedom. (当分析家庭、市民社会、国家、制度、习俗、法律或社会自由时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
**Sittlichkeit** is not simply “ethics.” It means ethical life as embodied in institutions and customs. Kantian morality emphasizes universal law and autonomy. Hegel argues that morality must become socially actual. Freedom requires not only inward intention but shared practices and institutions.  
  
This concept solves a major problem in moral philosophy. How does abstract moral law enter lived reality? Hegel’s answer: through ethical life.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Ethical life is the form in which freedom becomes a shared social reality rather than merely an inner moral demand. (伦理生活是自由成为共享社会现实的形式，而不只是内在道德要求。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Morality (道德性; de: Moralität)** concerns subjective intention and moral judgment; **Ethical Life (伦理生活; de: Sittlichkeit)** concerns institutionalized freedom. (道德性关涉主观意图与道德判断；伦理生活关涉制度化的自由。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** Sittlichkeit becomes a key source for later debates about liberal individualism, social embeddedness, civil society, state power, and communal norms. (伦理生活成为后来关于自由主义个人主义、社会嵌入性、市民社会、国家权力和共同体规范之争的重要来源。)  
  
### 19. History: The Problem of Rational Development over Time  
  
`History (历史; de: Geschichte)`  
**Definition:** the temporal process through which spirit, freedom, institutions, and rational forms develop. (精神、自由、制度和理性形式在其中发展的时间过程。)  
**Problem solved:** it makes temporality internal to reason rather than external chronology. (它使时间性成为理性的内在维度，而不是外在年代顺序。)  
**Why needed:** if spirit becomes actual through development, philosophy must think historical movement as conceptually meaningful. (如果精神通过发展成为现实，哲学就必须把历史运动思为具有概念意义。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing development, stages, institutions, conflict, progress, or historical consciousness. (当分析发展、阶段、制度、冲突、进步或历史意识时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
German Idealism gives history a philosophical function. History is not merely a record of events. It is the medium in which freedom becomes conscious and actual. This is one of the most consequential shifts in modern thought.  
  
This also creates danger. If history is treated as rationally progressing toward reconciliation, suffering may be absorbed into a totality too quickly. Later critique will attack exactly this danger.  
  
**Typical sentence:** History is not merely what happens in time; it is the medium through which spirit becomes actual. (历史不只是时间中发生的事，而是精神成为现实的媒介。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Chronology (年代顺序; el: χρόνος; de: Chronologie)** orders events by time; **History (历史; de: Geschichte)** gives events conceptual significance within development. (年代顺序按时间排列事件；历史则在发展中赋予事件概念意义。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** after German Idealism, philosophy can no longer treat reason as simply timeless. Marx, Nietzsche, historicism, hermeneutics, genealogy, and critical theory all inherit the problem of historical formation. (德国观念论之后，哲学无法再把理性简单视为无时间的。马克思、尼采、历史主义、解释学、谱系学和批判理论都继承了历史形成问题。)  
  
### 20. System: The Problem of Philosophical Completeness  
  
`System (体系; de: System)`  
**Definition:** an internally connected whole in which concepts derive meaning from their place in the total structure. (一个内部相连的整体，其中概念通过其在总体结构中的位置获得意义。)  
**Problem solved:** it prevents philosophy from remaining a collection of disconnected claims. (它防止哲学停留为互不相连的主张集合。)  
**Why needed:** if reason seeks unity, philosophy must show how its concepts belong together. (如果理性寻求统一，哲学就必须显示其概念如何彼此归属。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing the relation between parts and whole, sequence and necessity, or concept and totality. (当分析部分与整体、序列与必然性、概念与总体之间的关系时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
German Idealism is systematic because it treats concepts as internally connected. Being, essence, concept, nature, spirit, right, art, religion, and philosophy are not separate topics. They are moments of a total rational development.  
  
This systematic ambition gives German Idealism its power and its risk. It can show deep connections, but it may also over-totalize difference.  
  
**Typical sentence:** In a system, a concept receives its full meaning from its mediated place within the whole. (在体系中，一个概念从其在整体中的中介位置获得充分意义。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **System (体系; de: System)** differs from **Aggregate (集合; de: Aggregat)**. An aggregate is a collection of parts; a system is an internally articulated whole. (集合是部分的聚集；体系是内部展开的整体。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** later philosophy often defines itself by its relation to system. Marx transforms system into material social totality. Kierkegaard resists system in the name of existence. Nietzsche attacks systematic closure. Adorno attempts a negative dialectic against closed totality. (后来的哲学常通过其同体系的关系来定义自身。马克思把体系转化为物质社会总体；克尔凯郭尔以存在反抗体系；尼采攻击体系性封闭；阿多诺尝试以否定辩证法反对封闭总体。)  
  
### 21. The Tool-Map of German Idealism  
  
Use German Idealist vocabulary diagnostically. The core question is not only what something is, but how it becomes what it is through opposition, mediation, and development.  
  
**If the text asks how subjectivity becomes active**, look for **I (自我; de: Ich)**, **Self-Consciousness (自我意识; de: Selbstbewusstsein)**, and **Not-I (非我; de: Nicht-Ich)**.  
(如果文本追问主体性如何成为主动者，应寻找自我、自我意识与非我问题。)  
  
**If the text asks how opposition produces development**, look for **Negation (否定; de: Negation)**, **Contradiction (矛盾; de: Widerspruch)**, and **Dialectic (辩证法; de: Dialektik)**.  
(如果文本追问对立如何产生发展，应寻找否定、矛盾与辩证法问题。)  
  
**If the text asks how something is transformed without being erased**, look for **Aufhebung (扬弃; de: Aufhebung)**.  
(如果文本追问某物如何被转化而不被抹除，应寻找扬弃问题。)  
  
**If the text asks how identity depends on relation**, look for **Mediation (中介; de: Vermittlung)** and **Recognition (承认; de: Anerkennung)**.  
(如果文本追问同一性如何依赖关系，应寻找中介与承认问题。)  
  
**If the text asks how reason becomes social and historical**, look for **Spirit (精神; de: Geist)**, **Ethical Life (伦理生活; de: Sittlichkeit)**, and **History (历史; de: Geschichte)**.  
(如果文本追问理性如何成为社会的和历史的，应寻找精神、伦理生活与历史问题。)  
  
**If the text asks whether freedom is merely formal or actually realized**, look for **Freedom (自由; de: Freiheit)**, **Actuality (现实性; de: Wirklichkeit)**, and **Institution (制度; de: Institution)**.  
(如果文本追问自由只是形式上的还是已经现实化，应寻找自由、现实性与制度问题。)  
  
**If the text asks how concepts belong together**, look for **Concept (概念; de: Begriff)**, **System (体系; de: System)**, and **Absolute (绝对者; de: das Absolute)**.  
(如果文本追问概念如何彼此归属，应寻找概念、体系与绝对者问题。)  
  
### 22. The Genealogical Point of Part 5  
  
German Idealism transforms philosophy from a critique of conditions into a logic of development. Kant had shown that knowledge depends on conditions of possible experience. German Idealism asks whether those conditions themselves must be understood through activity, opposition, recognition, and history.  
  
The guiding thesis is:  
  
**German Idealist language turns reason into development: to understand a concept is to follow its movement through negation, mediation, contradiction, recognition, and historical actualization.**  
(德国观念论语言把理性转化为发展：理解一个概念，就是追踪它通过否定、中介、矛盾、承认和历史现实化而展开的运动。)  
  
This grammar will shape nearly everything that follows. Marx will transform dialectic into a critique of labor, capital, class, ideology, and alienation. Nietzsche will reject systematic reconciliation and turn critique toward value, morality, and force. Phenomenology will inherit the problem of consciousness but redirect it toward lived experience. Critical theory will inherit contradiction, mediation, and social totality. Foucault and genealogy will reject the idea of one rational totality, but retain the suspicion that concepts have histories and that what appears immediate is historically produced.  
  
The German Idealist question remains one of the central tools of philosophical reading:  
  
**What process, opposition, or mediation had to occur for this concept, institution, or form of life to become what it is?**  
(为了使这个概念、制度或生活形式成为其所是，必须发生什么过程、对立或中介？)  
  
## Part 6. Marx and Nietzsche: Suspicion, Value, Genealogy  
  
This chapter explains how nineteenth-century critique transforms German Idealism. Hegel had made reason historical through **Spirit**, **Dialectic**, **Mediation**, **Recognition**, and **Aufhebung**. Marx and Nietzsche inherit this historical grammar, but they redirect it against idealist reconciliation. Their question is sharper: **what material, social, bodily, affective, and power-laden forces produce the ideas that present themselves as truth?** (那些自称为真理的观念，是由哪些物质、社会、身体、情感和权力力量生产出来的？)  
  
This is the emergence of a language of suspicion. Philosophy no longer asks only whether a claim is true, valid, or rationally mediated. It asks what a claim **does**, whom it serves, what it conceals, and how it was historically produced. **Genealogy** names a historical technique that traces the evolution of ideas, questions their “natural” emergence, and exposes contingent power-relations shaping them; this chapter expands that function into a broader critical toolkit.  
  
The operational use of this chapter is direct: use Marxian and Nietzschean vocabulary when the issue is not merely **meaning**, but **production, domination, valuation, concealment, and historical formation**. (当问题不只是意义，而是生产、支配、赋值、遮蔽与历史形成时，应使用马克思与尼采式词汇。)  
  
### 1. The Problem-Situation: From Idealist Mediation to Material and Genealogical Critique  
  
German Idealism had argued that concepts develop through negation, contradiction, and mediation. Marx accepts this dynamic structure, but rejects the priority of **Spirit (精神; de: Geist)**. What develops historically is not first pure spirit, but social life organized through labor, production, class, property, and material relations.  
  
Nietzsche rejects a different idealist inheritance. He distrusts philosophical claims to pure reason, disinterested truth, universal morality, and metaphysical origin. For him, values have histories. Moral concepts are not simply discovered; they are created, inverted, imposed, internalized, and weaponized.  
  
The chapter therefore has two connected axes:  
  
**Marxian critique:** ideas must be understood through material production, labor, class, capital, and ideology. (马克思式批判：观念必须通过物质生产、劳动、阶级、资本和意识形态来理解。)  
  
**Nietzschean genealogy:** values must be understood through force, resentment, life, interpretation, and will to power. (尼采式谱系学：价值必须通过力量、怨恨、生命、解释和权力意志来理解。)  
  
Their shared problem is:  
  
**What appears rational, moral, or natural may be the historical effect of domination, need, struggle, or force.**  
(看似理性、道德或自然的东西，可能是支配、需要、斗争或力量的历史效果。)  
  
This does not mean that every truth-claim is automatically false. It means that critique must examine the conditions under which truth-claims become authoritative.  
  
### 2. Materialism: The Problem of Reversing Idealism  
  
`Materialism (唯物主义; de: Materialismus)`  
**Definition:** the view that social life, consciousness, and ideas must be explained through material conditions and practices rather than through pure thought alone. (认为社会生活、意识和观念必须通过物质条件与实践来解释，而不能只通过纯粹思想来解释的观点。)  
**Problem solved:** it reverses the idealist tendency to treat consciousness or spirit as primary. (它反转观念论把意识或精神视为首要者的倾向。)  
**Why needed:** ideas do not float above life; they arise within concrete forms of production, need, labor, and social relation. (观念并不漂浮在生活之上；它们产生于生产、需要、劳动和社会关系的具体形式之中。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing how social reality shapes consciousness, values, law, politics, religion, or philosophy. (当分析社会现实如何塑造意识、价值、法律、政治、宗教或哲学时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Marxian materialism is not merely the claim that matter exists. It is a method of explanation. It asks how human beings reproduce their lives, how labor is organized, how property is distributed, how institutions stabilize domination, and how ideas express or conceal these relations.  
  
This is a major shift in philosophical grammar. Instead of beginning with the self-conscious subject, the concept, or spirit, Marx begins from social production. Human beings must eat, work, cooperate, reproduce, exchange, and struggle. Thought arises within these conditions.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Materialism asks how forms of consciousness are produced by forms of life. (唯物主义追问意识形式如何由生活形式生产出来。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Materialism (唯物主义; de: Materialismus)** contrasts with **Idealism (观念论; de: Idealismus)**. Idealism explains reality through thought, spirit, or concept; materialism explains thought through social and material reality. (观念论通过思想、精神或概念解释现实；唯物主义通过社会和物质现实解释思想。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** materialism transforms the Hegelian problem of mediation. Mediation is no longer primarily conceptual; it becomes economic, social, institutional, and practical. (唯物主义改造了黑格尔的中介问题。中介不再首先是概念性的，而是经济的、社会的、制度的和实践的。)  
  
### 3. Historical Materialism: The Problem of History as Production  
  
`Historical Materialism (历史唯物主义; de: historischer Materialismus)`  
**Definition:** the method that explains historical development through material production, social relations, class struggle, and changing modes of life. (通过物质生产、社会关系、阶级斗争和生活方式的变化来解释历史发展的方法。)  
**Problem solved:** it gives history a material logic rather than a purely spiritual or moral narrative. (它为历史提供一种物质逻辑，而不是纯精神或道德叙事。)  
**Why needed:** historical change cannot be adequately explained by ideas alone if those ideas are rooted in material organization. (如果观念根植于物质组织，仅靠观念无法充分解释历史变化。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing how forms of society generate forms of consciousness, conflict, and transformation. (当分析社会形式如何生成意识形式、冲突和转化时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Historical materialism is a tool for reading history against its own self-description. A society may describe itself through religion, right, liberty, nation, morality, or progress. Historical materialism asks what material relations make these descriptions possible and useful.  
  
It is therefore not simply economic reductionism. Its deeper function is diagnostic: it reads ideals through their social basis.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Historical materialism treats ideas as historically effective, but not as historically self-sufficient. (历史唯物主义认为观念具有历史效力，但并不具有历史上的自足性。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Historical Materialism (历史唯物主义; de: historischer Materialismus)** differs from **Chronological History (年代史; de: Chronologie)**. Chronology orders events in time; historical materialism analyzes the material relations that make historical forms possible. (年代史按时间排列事件；历史唯物主义分析使历史形式成为可能的物质关系。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** history becomes a field of production and conflict rather than the self-unfolding of spirit. Later social theory, critical theory, and ideology critique inherit this method. (历史成为生产与冲突的场域，而不再是精神的自我展开。后来的社会理论、批判理论和意识形态批判继承了这一方法。)  
  
### 4. Labor: The Problem of Human Self-Production  
  
`Labor (劳动; de: Arbeit)`  
**Definition:** the practical activity through which human beings transform nature, produce goods, and form themselves socially. (人类借以改造自然、生产物品并在社会中形成自身的实践活动。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains human life as productive activity rather than mere contemplation or consciousness. (它把人类生活解释为生产性活动，而不只是沉思或意识。)  
**Why needed:** human beings do not merely interpret the world; they materially reproduce and transform it. (人类不只是解释世界；他们还物质地再生产并改造世界。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing production, social formation, self-realization, exploitation, or alienation. (当分析生产、社会形成、自我实现、剥削或异化时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Labor is Marx’s decisive reworking of Hegelian activity. German Idealism made subjectivity active; Marx makes activity practical and material. Labor is not merely economic effort. It is the process by which human beings objectify their powers in the world.  
  
This gives labor a double character. It can be self-realizing: human beings recognize themselves in what they produce. But under alienated conditions, labor becomes domination: the worker’s own activity returns as an alien power.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Labor is the practical mediation through which human beings transform nature and themselves. (劳动是人类改造自然并改造自身的实践中介。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Labor (劳动; de: Arbeit)** differs from **Work as mere toil (辛劳; en: toil)**. Labor is a social and formative activity, not only physical effort. (劳动是一种社会性和形成性的活动，而不只是体力辛劳。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** labor transforms the idealist problem of self-realization into a material problem of production, ownership, and alienation. (劳动把观念论的自我实现问题转化为生产、所有权和异化的物质问题。)  
  
### 5. Praxis: The Problem of Transformative Activity  
  
`Praxis (实践; el: πρᾶξις; de: Praxis)`  
**Definition:** practical, world-transforming activity in which theory and action are inseparable. (理论与行动不可分离的、改造世界的实践活动。)  
**Problem solved:** it overcomes the split between interpreting the world and changing it. (它克服解释世界与改变世界之间的分裂。)  
**Why needed:** critique must not remain contemplative if the conditions it diagnoses are practical and social. (如果批判所诊断的条件是实践的和社会的，批判就不能停留在沉思层面。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing revolutionary action, social transformation, embodied theory, or practice-based knowledge. (当分析革命行动、社会转化、具身理论或基于实践的知识时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Praxis is not simply “practice” in the everyday sense. It means transformative activity through which social reality is made and remade. In Marxian usage, praxis challenges philosophy that only contemplates or interprets.  
  
This does not make theory irrelevant. It makes theory accountable to practice. A theory of society must be tested by whether it grasps and transforms the relations it analyzes.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Praxis is theory become materially effective through transformative action. (实践是通过转化性行动而获得物质效力的理论。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Praxis (实践; de: Praxis)** differs from **Theory (理论; el: θεωρία; de: Theorie)** when theory is isolated from action. Praxis unites understanding and transformation. (当理论脱离行动时，实践与理论不同；实践统一理解与转化。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** praxis becomes central for Marxism, critical pedagogy, liberation theory, and political philosophy. It turns philosophical critique into a question of transformation. (实践成为马克思主义、批判教育学、解放理论和政治哲学的核心。它把哲学批判转化为转化问题。)  
  
### 6. Commodity: The Problem of Social Relations Appearing as Things  
  
`Commodity (商品; de: Ware)`  
**Definition:** an object produced for exchange within a market relation. (在市场关系中为交换而生产的对象。)  
**Problem solved:** it reveals how social labor appears in objectified form. (它揭示社会劳动如何以对象化形式显现。)  
**Why needed:** capitalism does not present itself first as domination; it presents itself as a world of things for exchange. (资本主义首先并不以支配的形式呈现自身，而是以可交换物的世界呈现自身。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing how market objects conceal the social relations that produced them. (当分析市场对象如何遮蔽生产它们的社会关系时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
The commodity is not just an economic item. It is a philosophical diagnostic object. It shows how relations between people can appear as relations between things. The table, coat, phone, or coin seems to carry value naturally, but its value depends on social labor and exchange relations.  
  
This is why commodity analysis is a model of critique. It takes what appears ordinary and shows the hidden social structure inside it.  
  
**Typical sentence:** The commodity is a thing-form in which social relations of labor appear as properties of objects. (商品是一种物的形式，其中劳动的社会关系表现为对象的属性。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Use-Value (使用价值; de: Gebrauchswert)** concerns the usefulness of a thing; **Exchange-Value (交换价值; de: Tauschwert)** concerns its value in exchange. (使用价值关涉物的有用性；交换价值关涉物在交换中的价值。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** commodity analysis prepares later critiques of reification, consumer society, spectacle, and neoliberal subjectivity. (商品分析为后来的物化、消费社会、景观和新自由主义主体性批判做准备。)  
  
### 7. Value: The Problem of Social Measurement  
  
`Value (价值; de: Wert)`  
**Definition:** the social form through which labor, usefulness, exchange, or moral worth is measured and ranked. (劳动、有用性、交换或道德价值被衡量和排序的社会形式。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains how different things become comparable. (它解释不同事物如何变得可比较。)  
**Why needed:** exchange requires a common measure, but that measure is socially produced rather than naturally visible. (交换需要共同尺度，但这一尺度是社会生产出来的，而不是自然可见的。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing equivalence, ranking, exchange, moral hierarchy, or social evaluation. (当分析等价、排序、交换、道德等级或社会评价时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Value is the bridge between Marx and Nietzsche. For Marx, value is tied to labor, exchange, and capitalist social relations. For Nietzsche, value is tied to life, force, interpretation, and the creation of moral hierarchies. Both ask the same dangerous question: **who or what produces value?** (谁或什么生产价值？)  
  
This makes value a critical rather than neutral concept. What presents itself as valuable may be the effect of labor relations, moral inversion, priestly power, ressentiment, or social domination.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Value is not simply found; it is produced, measured, imposed, and contested. (价值并不是简单被发现的；它被生产、衡量、强加并争夺。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Economic Value (经济价值; de: ökonomischer Wert)** concerns exchange and labor; **Moral Value (道德价值; de: moralischer Wert)** concerns evaluation of life, action, and character. (经济价值关涉交换与劳动；道德价值关涉对生命、行动和品格的评价。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** value becomes a site of suspicion. Critique asks whether value expresses life, labor, domination, resentment, or institutional power. (价值成为怀疑的场所。批判追问价值表达的是生命、劳动、支配、怨恨，还是制度权力。)  
  
### 8. Capital: The Problem of Self-Expanding Value  
  
`Capital (资本; de: Kapital)`  
**Definition:** value that circulates, accumulates, and expands through social relations of production and exchange. (通过生产与交换的社会关系而流通、积累并扩张的价值。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains capitalism not as a mere collection of goods, but as a dynamic system of value expansion. (它把资本主义解释为价值扩张的动态系统，而不只是物品集合。)  
**Why needed:** capitalist domination operates through impersonal structures as much as through direct command. (资本主义支配既通过非人格结构运作，也通过直接命令运作。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing accumulation, exploitation, wage labor, commodity circulation, or systemic compulsion. (当分析积累、剥削、雇佣劳动、商品流通或系统性强制时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Capital is not merely money. Money becomes capital when it is used to generate more value. Capital is therefore a process, not just a thing. It appears in objects, factories, wages, machines, prices, debts, and markets, but its logic is expansion.  
  
This is why Marxian critique targets structures rather than only intentions. The capitalist may be personally moral, but capital as a social relation compels accumulation, competition, extraction, and expansion.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Capital is value in motion, organizing social life according to the imperative of accumulation. (资本是在运动中的价值，它按照积累命令组织社会生活。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Money (货币; de: Geld)** can mediate exchange; **Capital (资本; de: Kapital)** uses exchange to expand value. (货币可以中介交换；资本则利用交换来扩张价值。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** capital becomes a model for later analyses of systems that operate behind individual intentions: bureaucracy, technology, media, platforms, data economies, and institutional power. (资本成为后来分析那些在个人意图背后运作的系统的模型：官僚制、技术、媒体、平台、数据经济和制度权力。)  
  
### 9. Class: The Problem of Structured Social Conflict  
  
`Class (阶级; de: Klasse)`  
**Definition:** a social group defined by its position within relations of production, ownership, and labor. (由其在生产、所有权和劳动关系中的位置所定义的社会群体。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains social conflict as structurally produced rather than merely personal or moral. (它把社会冲突解释为结构性生产的，而不只是个人或道德问题。)  
**Why needed:** capitalism divides people according to their relation to property, labor, and surplus extraction. (资本主义根据人与财产、劳动和剩余榨取的关系来划分人群。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing exploitation, political struggle, social position, collective interest, or historical transformation. (当分析剥削、政治斗争、社会位置、集体利益或历史转化时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Class is not simply income level. It names a structural position. The worker sells labor-power. The capitalist owns or controls means of production. Their relation is not accidental; it is built into the mode of production.  
  
This makes class conflict an explanatory tool. Social antagonism is not merely a failure of harmony. It arises from contradictory positions within production.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Class names a structural position within production, not merely a lifestyle or income bracket. (阶级命名生产中的结构位置，而不只是生活方式或收入层级。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Class (阶级; de: Klasse)** differs from **Status (地位; de: Stand/Status)**. Status concerns rank, honor, or social recognition; class concerns position in material relations of production. (地位关涉等级、荣誉或社会承认；阶级关涉物质生产关系中的位置。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** class analysis converts history into conflict over production, ownership, and social power. Later theory will complicate this through race, gender, coloniality, bureaucracy, and culture, but class remains a basic diagnostic tool. (阶级分析把历史转化为围绕生产、所有权与社会权力的冲突。后来的理论会通过种族、性别、殖民性、官僚制和文化使之复杂化，但阶级仍是基本诊断工具。)  
  
### 10. Ideology: The Problem of False Naturalness  
  
`Ideology (意识形态; de: Ideologie)`  
**Definition:** a system of representations, beliefs, or concepts that makes historically produced social relations appear natural, universal, or necessary. (一种使历史生产出来的社会关系显得自然、普遍或必然的表象、信念或概念系统。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains how domination can be reproduced through ideas that seem neutral or obvious. (它解释支配如何通过看似中立或显然的观念被再生产。)  
**Why needed:** social power does not operate only by force; it also operates by shaping what seems real, normal, and self-evident. (社会权力不只通过强力运作，也通过塑造何者显得真实、正常和不言自明来运作。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing concealment, naturalization, legitimation, false universality, or distorted consciousness. (当分析遮蔽、自然化、合法化、虚假普遍性或扭曲意识时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Ideology is one of the central instruments of suspicion. It does not mean simply “a set of political opinions.” In critical usage, ideology names the way social relations become misrecognized. A class society may present itself as free contract. Exploitation may appear as fair exchange. Historical privilege may appear as natural merit.  
  
The key diagnostic question is:  
  
**What social relation is being hidden by this apparently neutral concept?**  
(这个看似中立的概念遮蔽了什么社会关系？)  
  
**Typical sentence:** Ideology makes contingent social relations appear natural and necessary. (意识形态使偶然的社会关系显得自然且必然。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Error (错误; la: error)** is a false belief; **Ideology (意识形态; de: Ideologie)** is a socially structured form of misrecognition. (错误是虚假信念；意识形态是社会结构化的误认形式。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** ideology critique prepares later analyses of discourse, hegemony, normalization, and regimes of truth. Foucault will not simply use the same concept, but he will inherit the suspicion that knowledge and power are entangled. (意识形态批判为后来的话语、霸权、规范化和真理体制分析做准备。福柯不会简单使用同一概念，但他继承了知识与权力相互缠绕的怀疑。)  
  
### 11. Alienation: The Problem of One’s Own Power Returning as Foreign  
  
`Alienation (异化; de: Entfremdung)`  
**Definition:** a condition in which human activity, labor, product, social relation, or selfhood becomes foreign and dominating to the human beings who produced it. (人类活动、劳动、产品、社会关系或自我性对生产它们的人变得陌生且具有支配性的状态。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains how human self-expression becomes self-loss under distorted social conditions. (它解释在人类社会条件被扭曲时，自我表达如何变成自我丧失。)  
**Why needed:** exploitation is not only material deprivation; it is also estrangement from activity, product, others, and oneself. (剥削不只是物质剥夺，也是同活动、产品、他者和自身的疏离。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing labor that no longer belongs to the worker as meaningful self-activity. (当分析不再作为有意义自我活动而属于劳动者的劳动时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
**Usage layers:**  
1. **Hegelian use (黑格尔式用法):** **alienation / estrangement** names Spirit’s self-externalization and return through historical, social, and cultural forms. It can be part of development rather than merely loss. (在黑格尔那里，异化/疏离指精神通过历史、社会和文化形式的自我外化与回归。它可以是发展过程的一部分，而不只是丧失。)  
  
2. **Marxian use (马克思式用法):** alienation names the condition in which human powers, labor, products, social relations, or species-being return to human beings as foreign, dominating forces. (在马克思那里，异化指人的力量、劳动、产品、社会关系或类存在作为异己的支配力量返回到人自身面前。)  
  
3. **Contemporary transferable use (当代理论泛用法):** in existentialism, postcolonial theory, labor theory, digital life, and social criticism, alienation may describe estrangement from self, world, body, community, work, language, or agency. (在存在主义、后殖民理论、劳动理论、数字生活和社会批判中，异化可指人与自我、世界、身体、共同体、工作、语言或行动能力的疏离。)  
  
**Transfer rule:** before using **alienation**, ask what has become foreign: labor, self, world, social relation, body, language, or political agency. (转用规则：使用 alienation 之前，应先判断什么变成了异己之物：劳动、自我、世界、社会关系、身体、语言，还是政治行动能力。)  
  
**Misuse warning:** alienation is not merely sadness, loneliness, or dissatisfaction. It names a structural estrangement. (Alienation 不只是悲伤、孤独或不满，而是结构性疏离。)  
  
Marx inherits alienation from Hegel but materializes it. In capitalist production, the worker produces an object that belongs to another. The product confronts the worker as alien property. The labor process is externally imposed. Other workers become competitors. Human capacities are reduced to labor-power.  
  
Alienation therefore diagnoses more than unhappiness. It diagnoses a social structure in which human powers are objectified and then turned against human beings.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Alienation occurs when human powers are objectified in forms that dominate the humans who produced them. (当人类力量被对象化为反过来支配生产者的形式时，异化就发生了。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Objectification (对象化; de: Vergegenständlichung)** can be a normal expression of human activity; **Alienation (异化; de: Entfremdung)** occurs when objectification becomes estranged and dominating. (对象化可以是人类活动的正常表达；异化则发生在对象化变成疏离且支配性的形式时。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** alienation becomes a major diagnostic for modernity: work, bureaucracy, technology, consumption, sexuality, urban life, and even selfhood can be analyzed as alienated forms. (异化成为现代性的主要诊断工具：工作、官僚制、技术、消费、性、城市生活乃至自我性都可以作为异化形式来分析。)  
  
### 12. Fetishism: The Problem of Social Power Appearing as Object-Power  
  
`Fetishism (拜物教/物神性; de: Fetischismus)`  
**Definition:** the process by which social relations between people appear as relations between things or as powers of things themselves. (人与人之间的社会关系表现为物与物之间的关系，或表现为物自身力量的过程。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains why commodities seem to possess value naturally. (它解释为什么商品似乎天然具有价值。)  
**Why needed:** capitalist society hides social labor behind the object-form of commodities. (资本主义社会把社会劳动隐藏在商品的物形式背后。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing how objects, prices, markets, or institutions appear autonomous from the relations that produce them. (当分析对象、价格、市场或制度如何显得独立于生产它们的关系时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Fetishism is deeper than illusion. It is not simply that people mistakenly believe objects have value. In capitalism, social relations really do take the form of relations among commodities. The illusion is objective: it is built into the form of social life.  
  
This makes fetishism an advanced diagnostic tool. It shows that critique cannot merely correct ideas. It must analyze the social forms that generate those ideas.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Fetishism is the objective illusion through which social relations appear as properties of things. (物神性是社会关系表现为物的属性的客观幻象。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Ideology (意识形态; de: Ideologie)** concerns social misrecognition through ideas; **Fetishism (物神性; de: Fetischismus)** concerns misrecognition built into the object-form of exchange. (意识形态关涉通过观念发生的社会误认；物神性关涉内置于交换之物形式中的误认。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** fetishism prepares later analyses of spectacle, branding, consumer desire, platform value, and the aura of market objects. (物神性为后来的景观、品牌、消费欲望、平台价值和市场对象光环分析做准备。)  
  
### 13. Nietzschean Genealogy: The Problem of Morality’s History  
  
`Genealogy (谱系学; de: Genealogie; fr: généalogie)`  
**Definition:** a historical method that traces the contingent, conflictual, and power-laden formation of values, concepts, and truths. (一种追踪价值、概念和真理之偶然的、冲突性的、带有权力关系的形成过程的历史方法。)  
**Problem solved:** it breaks the illusion that moral concepts have pure, timeless, or natural origins. (它打破道德概念具有纯粹、永恒或自然起源的幻觉。)  
**Why needed:** values often hide the struggles and inversions through which they were produced. (价值常常遮蔽生产它们的斗争与反转。)  
**How to use:** use it when asking how a value came to appear self-evident, sacred, natural, or universal. (当追问某种价值如何显得不言自明、神圣、自然或普遍时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Genealogy is not ordinary history. It does not search for a pure origin. It searches for descent, conflict, accident, reinterpretation, and appropriation. It asks how concepts become authoritative.  
  
The genealogical question is not:  
  
**What is morality in itself?**  
(道德本身是什么？)  
  
It is:  
  
**Through what historical struggles did this morality become dominant?**  
(这种道德通过什么历史斗争成为支配性的？)  
  
**Typical sentence:** Genealogy does not recover a pure origin; it exposes the struggles through which an origin was invented. (谱系学并不恢复纯粹起源；它揭示所谓起源如何在斗争中被发明出来。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Origin (起源; de: Ursprung)** suggests a pure beginning; **Descent (来源/谱系; de: Herkunft)** suggests historical formation through multiple, impure lines. (起源暗示纯粹开端；来源/谱系暗示通过多重且不纯的线索形成的历史过程。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** Nietzsche’s genealogy becomes one of the main sources for Foucault’s later analysis of power, knowledge, discipline, and subjectivation. (尼采的谱系学成为福柯后来分析权力、知识、规训和主体化的主要来源之一。)  
  
### 14. Morality: The Problem of Value Disguised as Universality  
  
`Morality (道德; de: Moral)`  
**Definition:** a historically formed system of valuations, duties, prohibitions, and ideals. (一种历史形成的价值评估、义务、禁令和理想体系。)  
**Problem solved:** it gives social life normative order, but also conceals the forces that produced that order. (它为社会生活提供规范秩序，但也遮蔽生产这种秩序的力量。)  
**Why needed:** Nietzsche needs a concept that can be criticized not as false belief alone, but as a life-shaping system of valuation. (尼采需要一个概念，使道德能够作为塑造生命的价值系统被批判，而不只是作为虚假信念被批判。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing how good, evil, guilt, duty, purity, and responsibility are historically produced. (当分析善、恶、罪责、义务、纯洁和责任如何被历史生产时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Nietzsche does not simply ask whether moral rules are valid. He asks what kind of life they express. A morality may strengthen life, weaken it, discipline it, domesticate it, or turn it against itself.  
  
This is the key Nietzschean move: morality is interpreted physiologically, affectively, and historically. It is not only a set of rational propositions. It is a symptom.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Morality is not only a code of rules; it is a historical interpretation of life. (道德不只是一套规则，而是对生命的历史性解释。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Moral Justification (道德证成; en: moral justification)** asks whether a rule is valid; **Genealogical Critique (谱系学批判; de: genealogische Kritik)** asks what forces produced the rule and what kind of life it serves. (道德证成追问规则是否有效；谱系学批判追问什么力量生产了规则，以及它服务于何种生命。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** morality loses its innocence. It becomes an object of diagnosis rather than merely a source of judgment. (道德失去其天真性。它成为诊断对象，而不只是判断来源。)  
  
### 15. Master Morality and Slave Morality: The Problem of Inverted Value  
  
`Master Morality (主人道德; de: Herrenmoral)`  
**Definition:** a value-system created from strength, affirmation, rank, self-confidence, and noble self-description. (一种由力量、肯定、等级、自信和高贵的自我描述所创造的价值系统。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains morality as value-creation by those who affirm themselves. (它把道德解释为由肯定自身者所进行的价值创造。)  
**Why needed:** Nietzsche needs a contrast to morality based on resentment and negation. (尼采需要一个与基于怨恨和否定的道德相对照的概念。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing values formed by affirmation rather than reactive condemnation. (当分析由肯定而非反应性谴责形成的价值时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
`Slave Morality (奴隶道德; de: Sklavenmoral)`  
**Definition:** a value-system formed reactively by the weak, powerless, or resentful against the strong. (一种由弱者、无权者或怨恨者针对强者而反应性形成的价值系统。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains how weakness can become morally superior by redefining strength as evil. (它解释弱如何通过把强重新定义为恶而成为道德上的优越者。)  
**Why needed:** Nietzsche wants to show that values can be produced through inversion. (尼采想显示价值能够通过反转被生产出来。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing moral systems that define themselves by negating an enemy. (当分析通过否定敌人来定义自身的道德系统时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
The master/slave distinction is not a simple political sociology. It is a genealogy of value-creation. Master morality begins by affirming itself: “good” means noble, powerful, beautiful, high, self-affirming. Slave morality begins reactively: “evil” is first assigned to the powerful other; “good” then becomes whatever is harmless, humble, obedient, suffering, or meek.  
  
This is moral inversion. Value is produced by reversal.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Slave morality creates value by first condemning the other as evil and then defining itself as good. (奴隶道德首先把他者谴责为恶，然后把自身定义为善，从而创造价值。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Active Valuation (主动赋值; de: aktive Wertsetzung)** creates from affirmation; **Reactive Valuation (反应性赋值; de: reaktive Wertsetzung)** creates from negation. (主动赋值从肯定出发创造价值；反应性赋值从否定出发创造价值。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** values are no longer treated as self-evident moral facts. They become historical products of force, rank, resentment, and interpretation. (价值不再被视为不言自明的道德事实，而成为力量、等级、怨恨和解释的历史产物。)  
  
### 16. Ressentiment: The Problem of Reactive Affect  
  
`Ressentiment (怨恨; fr/de: ressentiment)`  
**Definition:** a reactive affect in which blocked power turns into moral condemnation, memory, and revenge through value-creation. (一种反应性情感，其中受阻的力量通过价值创造转化为道德谴责、记忆和复仇。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains how powerlessness can produce moral authority. (它解释无力如何能够生产道德权威。)  
**Why needed:** Nietzsche needs a psychological and historical mechanism for the inversion of values. (尼采需要一个心理和历史机制来解释价值反转。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing moral judgment as displaced revenge or reactive self-justification. (当把道德判断分析为被转移的复仇或反应性自我辩护时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
**Ressentiment** is not ordinary resentment. It is a structured incapacity to act outwardly that turns inward and becomes evaluative. Unable to discharge force directly, the subject reinterprets its own weakness as goodness and the other’s strength as evil.  
  
This makes ressentiment a concept for diagnosing moral language. It asks whether a moral claim expresses justice or a disguised desire to reverse impotence into superiority.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Ressentiment turns blocked action into moral judgment. (怨恨把受阻的行动转化为道德判断。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Anger (愤怒; de: Zorn)** may discharge itself directly; **Ressentiment (怨恨; fr/de: ressentiment)** preserves injury and transforms it into a value-system. (愤怒可能直接释放自身；怨恨保存伤害并把它转化为价值系统。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** ressentiment becomes a diagnostic tool for moralism, nationalism, identity conflicts, punitive politics, and cultural resentment. (怨恨成为诊断道德主义、民族主义、身份冲突、惩罚性政治和文化怨恨的工具。)  
  
### 17. Will to Power: The Problem of Force beneath Value  
  
`Will to Power (权力意志; de: Wille zur Macht)`  
**Definition:** the drive of life to expand, interpret, organize, overcome resistance, and impose form. (生命扩张、解释、组织、克服阻力并强加形式的驱力。)  
**Problem solved:** it gives Nietzsche a non-moral grammar for interpreting life, value, and thought. (它为尼采提供一种非道德的语法，用来解释生命、价值和思想。)  
**Why needed:** if values are historically produced, one must ask what forces produce and sustain them. (如果价值是历史生产出来的，就必须追问什么力量生产并维持这些价值。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing interpretation, domination, self-overcoming, valuation, or the force-character of life. (当分析解释、支配、自我超克、赋值或生命的力量特征时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
The will to power should not be reduced to crude desire for political domination. It is broader. It names the interpretive and formative force of life. Living beings do not merely survive; they organize, rank, appropriate, overcome, and create forms.  
  
This gives Nietzsche a way to read philosophy itself. A philosophy is not only a set of arguments. It is an expression of a type of life, a style of valuation, a will to impose order on becoming.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Will to power names the force by which life interprets, ranks, and gives form. (权力意志命名生命借以解释、排序并赋予形式的力量。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Will to Power (权力意志; de: Wille zur Macht)** differs from **Will as Choice (作为选择的意志; la: voluntas)**. It is not merely a faculty of decision but a dynamic of force and interpretation. (权力意志不同于作为选择能力的意志；它不是单纯决断能力，而是力量与解释的动态。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** force replaces rational ground as a tool of interpretation. Later genealogy and post-structuralism will inherit this suspicion toward neutral reason and stable origin. (力量取代理性根据成为解释工具。后来的谱系学和后结构主义会继承这种对中立理性和稳定起源的怀疑。)  
  
### 18. Perspective: The Problem of Situated Interpretation  
  
`Perspective (视角; de: Perspektive)`  
**Definition:** a situated mode of interpretation shaped by life, force, interest, and position. (一种由生命、力量、利益和位置塑造的处境化解释方式。)  
**Problem solved:** it challenges the ideal of a view from nowhere. (它挑战无位置视角的理想。)  
**Why needed:** knowledge is always interpreted from somewhere, by a form of life with particular drives and interests. (知识总是从某个位置被解释出来，并由具有特定驱力和利益的生命形式承担。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing objectivity, interpretation, value, standpoint, or the limits of neutrality. (当分析客观性、解释、价值、立场或中立性限度时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Nietzschean perspectivism does not simply mean that all views are equally false. It means that knowing is always situated and interpretive. There is no pure, disembodied, interest-free access to truth.  
  
This does not abolish evaluation. It changes how evaluation works. One asks which perspective is stronger, richer, more life-affirming, more comprehensive, or more honest about its own conditions.  
  
**Typical sentence:** A perspective is not a distortion added to knowledge from outside; it is the condition under which something becomes interpretable. (视角不是从外部添加给知识的扭曲，而是某物成为可解释之物的条件。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Perspective (视角; de: Perspektive)** differs from **Relativism (相对主义; de: Relativismus)**. Perspectivism denies view-from-nowhere neutrality; it does not necessarily deny all ranking among interpretations. (视角主义否认无位置的中立性，但不必然否认解释之间的一切排序。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** perspective prepares later standpoint theory, hermeneutics, phenomenology, psychoanalysis, and post-structural critique of neutral knowledge. (视角为后来的立场理论、解释学、现象学、精神分析和后结构主义对中立知识的批判做准备。)  
  
### 19. Interpretation: The Problem of Meaning as Force  
  
`Interpretation (解释; de: Auslegung/Interpretation)`  
**Definition:** the act of giving meaning, order, or value to what appears. (赋予显现之物以意义、秩序或价值的活动。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains meaning as produced rather than simply received. (它把意义解释为被生产出来的，而不只是被接受的。)  
**Why needed:** facts do not present their significance without a framework of valuation and interpretation. (事实并不会脱离价值和解释框架而自行呈现其意义。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing how a claim, object, event, or body is made meaningful. (当分析一个主张、对象、事件或身体如何被赋予意义时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
For Nietzsche, interpretation is not secondary. It is not merely what one does after encountering a neutral fact. Interpretation belongs to life’s activity. To perceive, classify, value, remember, punish, or philosophize is already to interpret.  
  
This makes truth less innocent. A truth may be an interpretation that has forgotten itself as interpretation.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Interpretation does not merely describe meaning; it produces the field in which meaning can appear. (解释并不只是描述意义；它生产意义能够显现的场域。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Description (描述; la: descriptio)** claims to state what is there; **Interpretation (解释; de: Auslegung)** gives form, relation, and value to what is there. (描述声称陈述在那里之物；解释则为在那里之物赋予形式、关系和价值。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** interpretation becomes a weapon against metaphysical immediacy. Later hermeneutics will universalize interpretation; Foucault will analyze discourse; Derrida will destabilize final meaning. (解释成为反对形而上学直接性的武器。后来的解释学会普遍化解释；福柯会分析话语；德里达会动摇最终意义。)  
  
### 20. Death of God: The Problem of Collapsed Transcendent Guarantee  
  
`Death of God (上帝之死; de: Tod Gottes)`  
**Definition:** the collapse of the transcendent guarantee for truth, morality, order, and meaning. (真理、道德、秩序与意义的超越保证的崩塌。)  
**Problem solved:** it names the historical crisis in which inherited values lose their metaphysical foundation. (它命名继承价值失去其形而上学基础的历史危机。)  
**Why needed:** modernity cannot simply continue using Christian-moral values after their theological ground has weakened. (现代性不能在其神学根据削弱之后仍简单继续使用基督教—道德价值。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing nihilism, secularization, value crisis, or the loss of ultimate foundation. (当分析虚无主义、世俗化、价值危机或终极根据丧失时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
The death of God is not mainly a claim about atheism. It is a diagnosis of European culture. If God was the highest guarantee of truth and value, then God’s death means the collapse of the metaphysical structure that supported morality, purpose, and order.  
  
This creates a dangerous opening. Either inherited values continue as empty habits, or new values must be created.  
  
**Typical sentence:** The death of God means that inherited values survive without the foundation that once authorized them. (上帝之死意味着继承下来的价值仍然存活，但其曾经的授权根据已经崩塌。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Atheism (无神论; de: Atheismus)** denies God’s existence; **Death of God (上帝之死; de: Tod Gottes)** diagnoses the cultural collapse of transcendent value-foundation. (无神论否认上帝存在；上帝之死诊断超越价值根据的文化性崩塌。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** this diagnosis prepares existentialism, nihilism, value-creation, and post-metaphysical philosophy. (这一诊断为存在主义、虚无主义、价值创造和后形而上学哲学做准备。)  
  
### 21. Nihilism: The Problem of Value after Foundation  
  
`Nihilism (虚无主义; la: nihil; de: Nihilismus)`  
**Definition:** the condition in which highest values lose binding force, meaning, or credibility. (最高价值丧失约束力、意义或可信性的状态。)  
**Problem solved:** it diagnoses the crisis produced when inherited values no longer persuade but no new values have been created. (它诊断继承价值不再具有说服力而新价值尚未被创造时产生的危机。)  
**Why needed:** critique of morality risks destroying meaning unless it also confronts value-creation. (道德批判如果不同时面对价值创造，就有摧毁意义的风险。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing collapse of meaning, exhaustion of values, cynicism, passive despair, or active revaluation. (当分析意义崩塌、价值枯竭、犬儒、消极绝望或积极重估时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Nihilism is not merely the belief that nothing matters. It is a historical condition. Values that once governed life lose authority, but the habits formed by those values remain. This produces passivity, resentment, exhaustion, or the opportunity for revaluation.  
  
Nietzsche distinguishes the danger of passive nihilism from the possibility of active nihilism. Passive nihilism collapses. Active nihilism clears space for new valuation.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Nihilism is not the absence of values, but the collapse of the authority of inherited values. (虚无主义不是没有价值，而是继承价值的权威崩塌。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Passive Nihilism (消极虚无主义; de: passiver Nihilismus)** resigns itself to meaninglessness; **Active Nihilism (积极虚无主义; de: aktiver Nihilismus)** destroys exhausted values in order to create new ones. (消极虚无主义屈从于无意义；积极虚无主义摧毁枯竭价值，以便创造新价值。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** nihilism becomes the central diagnosis of post-Christian, post-metaphysical modernity. Existentialism and post-structuralism both inherit this crisis. (虚无主义成为后基督教、后形而上学现代性的核心诊断。存在主义和后结构主义都继承了这一危机。)  
  
### 22. Revaluation: The Problem of Creating Values  
  
`Revaluation of Values (价值重估; de: Umwertung der Werte)`  
**Definition:** the critical reversal and creation of values after inherited moral hierarchies lose authority. (在继承的道德等级失去权威后，对价值进行批判性反转与创造。)  
**Problem solved:** it offers a response to nihilism that is creative rather than merely destructive. (它为虚无主义提供一种创造性而非单纯破坏性的回应。)  
**Why needed:** genealogy can expose value-origins, but life still requires valuation. (谱系学能够揭示价值起源，但生命仍然需要赋值。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing the transformation of moral hierarchies, the creation of new ideals, or the overcoming of nihilism. (当分析道德等级的转化、新理想的创造或虚无主义的克服时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Revaluation is the constructive side of Nietzsche’s critique. If values are not grounded in a transcendent order, they must be created. But creation is not arbitrary preference. It expresses a form of life, a strength, a style, a capacity to affirm becoming.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Revaluation does not merely reject old values; it asks what kind of life can create new ones. (价值重估不只是拒绝旧价值；它追问什么样的生命能够创造新价值。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Critique (批判; de: Kritik)** exposes limits; **Revaluation (价值重估; de: Umwertung)** creates a new hierarchy of value. (批判揭示限度；价值重估创造新的价值等级。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** critique becomes inseparable from creation. Later philosophies of liberation, aesthetics, existentialism, and political transformation will inherit this double demand. (批判与创造变得不可分离。后来的解放哲学、美学、存在主义和政治转化理论都会继承这一双重要求。)  
  
### 23. Suspicion: The Shared Method  
  
`Suspicion (怀疑/疑思; fr: soupçon; de: Verdacht)`  
**Definition:** a critical stance that reads surface meanings as symptoms of deeper forces, interests, conflicts, or formations. (一种批判立场，它把表层意义读作更深层力量、利益、冲突或形成过程的症状。)  
**Problem solved:** it prevents philosophy from accepting self-presentations at face value. (它防止哲学按表面自我呈现来接受事物。)
