**Why needed:** domination often speaks in the language of truth, morality, law, or nature. (支配常以真理、道德、法律或自然的语言说话。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing what a claim conceals, what interest it serves, or what historical process produced it. (当分析一个主张遮蔽什么、服务什么利益或由什么历史过程生产时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Marx and Nietzsche belong to different traditions, but both create a hermeneutics of suspicion. Marx asks what material relations hide behind ideas. Nietzsche asks what forces and affects hide behind values. Both refuse the innocence of philosophical language.  
  
The shared diagnostic question is:  
  
**What is this concept doing beneath what it says?**  
(这个概念在其所说内容之下正在做什么？)  
  
**Typical sentence:** Suspicion reads a concept not only by its meaning, but by its function, origin, and effects. (怀疑式阅读不仅根据概念的意义来读它，也根据其功能、来源和效果来读它。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Interpretation (解释; de: Interpretation)** asks what something means; **Suspicion (疑思; fr: soupçon)** asks what this meaning conceals or enables. (解释追问某物意味着什么；疑思追问这一意义遮蔽或促成了什么。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** suspicion prepares psychoanalysis, ideology critique, genealogy, discourse analysis, critical theory, and deconstruction. (疑思为精神分析、意识形态批判、谱系学、话语分析、批判理论和解构做准备。)  
  
### 24. The Tool-Map of Marx and Nietzsche  
  
Use this chapter diagnostically. The question is usually not only “Is this claim true?” but “What produced this claim, and what does it do?”  
  
**If the text asks how ideas arise from social life**, look for **Materialism (唯物主义; de: Materialismus)**, **Historical Materialism (历史唯物主义; de: historischer Materialismus)**, and **Praxis (实践; de: Praxis)**.  
(如果文本追问观念如何产生于社会生活，应寻找唯物主义、历史唯物主义和实践问题。)  
  
**If the text asks how human activity becomes social structure**, look for **Labor (劳动; de: Arbeit)**, **Objectification (对象化; de: Vergegenständlichung)**, and **Alienation (异化; de: Entfremdung)**.  
(如果文本追问人类活动如何成为社会结构，应寻找劳动、对象化和异化问题。)  
  
**If the text asks how capitalism hides itself**, look for **Commodity (商品; de: Ware)**, **Value (价值; de: Wert)**, **Capital (资本; de: Kapital)**, **Class (阶级; de: Klasse)**, and **Fetishism (物神性; de: Fetischismus)**.  
(如果文本追问资本主义如何遮蔽自身，应寻找商品、价值、资本、阶级和物神性问题。)  
  
**If the text asks how domination is reproduced through ideas**, look for **Ideology (意识形态; de: Ideologie)** and **False Naturalness (虚假自然性; en: false naturalness)**.  
(如果文本追问支配如何通过观念被再生产，应寻找意识形态与虚假自然性问题。)  
  
**If the text asks how moral values were historically produced**, look for **Genealogy (谱系学; de: Genealogie)**, **Morality (道德; de: Moral)**, **Master Morality (主人道德; de: Herrenmoral)**, and **Slave Morality (奴隶道德; de: Sklavenmoral)**.  
(如果文本追问道德价值如何被历史生产，应寻找谱系学、道德、主人道德和奴隶道德问题。)  
  
**If the text asks what affective force lies beneath moral judgment**, look for **Ressentiment (怨恨; fr/de: ressentiment)**.  
(如果文本追问道德判断之下有什么情感力量，应寻找怨恨问题。)  
  
**If the text asks how value is created after metaphysical foundations collapse**, look for **Death of God (上帝之死; de: Tod Gottes)**, **Nihilism (虚无主义; de: Nihilismus)**, and **Revaluation of Values (价值重估; de: Umwertung der Werte)**.  
(如果文本追问形而上学根据崩塌之后价值如何被创造，应寻找上帝之死、虚无主义和价值重估问题。)  
  
**If the text asks why neutrality is suspicious**, look for **Perspective (视角; de: Perspektive)**, **Interpretation (解释; de: Interpretation)**, and **Will to Power (权力意志; de: Wille zur Macht)**.  
(如果文本追问为什么中立性值得怀疑，应寻找视角、解释和权力意志问题。)  
  
### 25. The Genealogical Point of Part 6  
  
Marx and Nietzsche transform the meaning of critique. German Idealism had shown that concepts develop through negation, mediation, and history. Marx turns this into a critique of material production, labor, class, ideology, and capital. Nietzsche turns it into a genealogy of morality, ressentiment, value, and force.  
  
The guiding thesis is:  
  
**The language of suspicion turns philosophy against the innocence of its own concepts: to understand an idea is to ask what material relations, affects, powers, and historical struggles produced it and allow it to function as truth.**  
(怀疑的语言使哲学反过来审问自身概念的天真性：理解一个观念，就是追问什么物质关系、情感、权力和历史斗争生产了它，并使它能够作为真理运作。)  
  
This chapter is the bridge to twentieth-century critique. Phenomenology will return to experience, but cannot ignore historical suspicion. Heidegger will reopen Being, but under the shadow of metaphysical history. Critical theory will combine Marxian contradiction with social diagnosis. Foucault will radicalize genealogy into an analysis of **Power/Knowledge (权力/知识; fr: savoir-pouvoir; en: power/knowledge)**, the inseparability of power relations and knowledge production. Derrida will expose how conceptual hierarchies depend on exclusions and traces.  
  
The Marx-Nietzsche question remains one of the most powerful tools for philosophical reading:  
  
**What appears as truth, morality, or nature here, and what historical force made it appear that way?**  
(这里什么东西表现为真理、道德或自然？又是什么历史力量使它以这种方式显现？)  
  
## Part 7. Phenomenology: Intentionality, World, Lived Experience  
  
This chapter explains how phenomenology transforms the modern problem of knowledge. Early modern philosophy asked how the subject represents the object. Kant asked what conditions make experience possible. German Idealism made those conditions dynamic and historical. Marx and Nietzsche introduced suspicion toward concepts, values, and consciousness itself. Phenomenology enters this field with a different methodological demand: **return to the things themselves**. (回到事情本身。)  
  
This does not mean returning to naive realism. It means returning to how things are given in experience before theoretical abstractions, natural-scientific reductions, or inherited metaphysical assumptions take over. The central vocabulary is **Phenomenology**, **Intentionality**, **Consciousness**, **Noesis**, **Noema**, **Epoché**, **Reduction**, **Natural Attitude**, **Lifeworld**, **Horizon**, **Constitution**, **Givenness**, **Embodiment**, and **Perception**. **Intentionality** names the Husserlian claim that consciousness is always about something, **Epoché** names the suspension of the natural attitude, and **Lebenswelt** names the pre-reflective everyday world of lived experience.  
  
The operational function of this chapter is precise: use phenomenological vocabulary when the issue is **how something appears, is meant, is given, or is lived before it becomes an object of explanation**. (当问题是某物如何显现、被意指、被给予或被生活，而不是它如何被外部解释时，应使用现象学词汇。)  
  
### 1. The Problem-Situation: From Explanation to Description  
  
Phenomenology begins from dissatisfaction with inherited philosophical alternatives. Realism treats the object as simply there. Idealism risks making the object dependent on the subject. Psychologism reduces logic or meaning to mental events. Naturalism reduces consciousness to a fact among facts. Historicist suspicion may explain concepts through social or historical conditions but can overlook the structure of experience itself.  
  
Phenomenology asks a prior question:  
  
**How is anything given as meaningful in experience at all?**  
(任何东西究竟如何在经验中作为有意义之物被给予？)  
  
This question shifts philosophical attention from causal explanation to descriptive clarification. The first task is not to explain experience from outside, but to describe its structures from within. Consciousness is not treated as a sealed container filled with ideas. It is directed, relational, temporal, embodied, and world-involved.  
  
Phenomenology therefore changes the basic philosophical grammar:  
  
Not: **subject inside, object outside**.  
(不是：主体在内，客体在外。)  
  
But: **intentional relation, meaningful givenness, world-involvement**.  
(而是：意向关系、有意义的给予性、在世界中的牵连。)  
  
**Typical sentence:** Phenomenology does not begin by explaining consciousness causally; it describes how things are given to consciousness as meaningful. (现象学并不首先以因果方式解释意识；它描述事物如何作为有意义之物被给予给意识。)  
  
### 2. Phenomenology: The Problem of Appearing  
  
`Phenomenology (现象学; el: φαινόμενον; de: Phänomenologie)`  
**Definition:** the disciplined description of the structures through which things appear or are given in experience. (对事物在经验中显现或被给予之结构的有规训描述。)  
**Problem solved:** it provides a method for analyzing experience without immediately reducing it to psychology, natural science, metaphysics, or social explanation. (它提供一种方法，使经验能够被分析，而不立即被化约为心理学、自然科学、形而上学或社会解释。)  
**Why needed:** philosophical concepts often presuppose experience while failing to describe how experience is structured. (哲学概念常常预设经验，却没有描述经验如何被结构化。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing the mode of appearing of an object, value, body, world, other person, memory, time, or meaning. (当分析对象、价值、身体、世界、他者、记忆、时间或意义的显现方式时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Phenomenology is a method before it is a doctrine. It asks for careful description. A table, a melody, a promise, a pain, a number, a memory, a tool, a face, and a political demand do not appear in the same way. Each has its own mode of givenness.  
  
This is why phenomenological language is useful. It prevents philosophy from treating all objects as if they were physical things simply placed before a detached observer. The experienced world is richer than the object-world of natural science.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Phenomenology asks not only what appears, but how it appears as what it is. (现象学不只问什么显现，而是问它如何作为其所是者而显现。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Phenomenology (现象学; de: Phänomenologie)** differs from **Natural Explanation (自然解释; de: natürliche Erklärung)**. Natural explanation explains an event by causal mechanisms; phenomenology describes the structure of its appearing. (自然解释通过因果机制解释事件；现象学描述其显现结构。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** phenomenology reactivates the Greek problem of **Appearance (显现; el: φαινόμενον)**, but without simply opposing appearance to truth. Appearance becomes the very field in which meaning and objectivity must be investigated. (现象学重新激活希腊的显现问题，但并不简单把显现同真理对立起来。显现成为意义与客观性必须被考察的场域。)  
  
### 3. Intentionality: The Problem of Consciousness as Directedness  
  
`Intentionality (意向性/指向性; la: intentio; de: Intentionalität)`  
**Definition:** the structure by which consciousness is always consciousness of something. (意识总是关于某物的意识这一结构。)  
**Problem solved:** it breaks the model of consciousness as an inner container of mental states. (它打破把意识看作心灵状态之内部容器的模型。)  
**Why needed:** experience is not first an inner event and then later related to an object; it is object-directed from the start. (经验并非首先是内部事件，然后才同对象发生关系；它从一开始就是指向对象的。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing how thinking, perceiving, remembering, desiring, judging, fearing, or imagining are directed toward something. (当分析思考、知觉、记忆、欲望、判断、恐惧或想象如何指向某物时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Intentionality is the central phenomenological tool. It replaces the picture of consciousness as an enclosed inner theater. Consciousness is always stretched toward something: a tree, a number, a friend, a possibility, a loss, a future, a value, a task, a world.  
  
This means that consciousness and object are not first two isolated substances that later need to be connected. The relation is primary. Consciousness is relational in its very structure.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Consciousness is not a container of representations; it is a directed relation toward what is meant. (意识不是表象容器，而是朝向被意指之物的指向性关系。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Intentional Object (意向对象; de: intentionaler Gegenstand)** is not necessarily a real physical object. It is the object as meant, intended, remembered, feared, imagined, or judged. (意向对象不必然是现实物理对象，而是作为被意指、被记忆、被恐惧、被想象或被判断之物的对象。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** intentionality transforms early modern representation. Instead of asking how an inner idea corresponds to an external object, phenomenology asks how the object is intended and given in the act of consciousness. (意向性改造近代表象问题。现象学不再首先追问内部观念如何符合外部对象，而是追问对象如何在意识活动中被意指和被给予。)  
  
### 4. Consciousness: The Problem of Lived Directedness  
  
`Consciousness (意识; la: conscientia; de: Bewusstsein)`  
**Definition:** the field of lived directedness in which objects, meanings, values, and worlds are given. (对象、意义、价值与世界在其中被给予的被生活的指向性场域。)  
**Problem solved:** it allows experience to be analyzed as meaningful rather than as a mere sequence of mental events. (它使经验能够作为有意义的结构被分析，而不是作为心灵事件的单纯序列。)  
**Why needed:** psychology may explain mental events causally, but philosophy must describe the meaningful structure of experiencing. (心理学可以因果性地解释心灵事件，但哲学必须描述经验活动的意义结构。)  
**How to use:** use it when the issue is the givenness of objects, the structure of experience, or the relation between meaning and subjectivity. (当问题涉及对象的给予性、经验结构或意义与主体性之间的关系时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Phenomenological consciousness is not merely private interiority. It is the site where world, object, body, time, and others appear. This does not mean that consciousness creates everything arbitrarily. It means that philosophical analysis must attend to how things become present as meaningful within lived experience.  
  
This also changes the status of subjectivity. The subject is not merely a point of certainty, as in the early modern cogito. Nor is it only a social-historical product, as in some suspicious readings. It is the field of intentional life in which meanings are disclosed.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Consciousness is lived directedness toward a meaningful world. (意识是朝向有意义世界的被生活的指向性。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Consciousness (意识; de: Bewusstsein)** differs from **Self-Consciousness (自我意识; de: Selbstbewusstsein)**. Consciousness is directed toward something; self-consciousness involves reflexive relation to oneself. (意识指向某物；自我意识涉及同自身的反身关系。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** phenomenology does not abandon the modern subject; it redescribes subjectivity as intentional, temporal, embodied, and world-involved. (现象学并不抛弃现代主体，而是把主体性重述为意向性的、时间性的、具身的和牵连于世界的。)  
  
### 5. Noesis and Noema: The Problem of Act and Meaning  
  
`Noesis (意向活动; el: νόησις; de: Noesis)`  
**Definition:** the act-side of intentional consciousness, such as perceiving, judging, remembering, imagining, or valuing. (意向意识的活动面，如知觉、判断、记忆、想象或赋值。)  
**Problem solved:** it distinguishes the activity of meaning from the meant content. (它把意义活动同被意指内容区分开来。)  
**Why needed:** the same object can be intended through different acts. (同一个对象可以通过不同活动被意指。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing the mode of conscious act through which something is given. (当分析某物通过何种意识活动被给予时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
`Noema (意向内容/意向对象; el: νόημα; de: Noema)`  
**Definition:** the object or sense as intended in an intentional act. (在意向活动中作为被意指者的对象或意义。)  
**Problem solved:** it distinguishes the object as meant from the psychological act of meaning it. (它把作为被意指者的对象同意指它的心理活动区分开来。)  
**Why needed:** phenomenology must analyze not only acts, but what appears in and through those acts. (现象学不仅要分析活动，也要分析在活动中并通过活动显现的东西。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing the object as perceived, remembered, imagined, judged, or valued. (当分析作为被知觉、被记忆、被想象、被判断或被赋值的对象时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
The **noesis/noema** distinction gives phenomenology precision. A tree can be perceived, remembered, imagined, doubted, photographed, desired, feared, or scientifically classified. The object may be “the same tree,” but its noematic sense changes according to the noetic act.  
  
This distinction prevents crude subjectivism. Phenomenology is not merely interested in inner acts. It is interested in the correlation between act and sense.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Noesis names the intending act; noema names the object as intended. (Noesis 命名意向活动；noema 命名作为被意指者的对象。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Psychological Event (心理事件; en: psychological event)** is a factual occurrence in mental life; **Noetic-Noematic Correlation (意向活动—意向内容相关性; de: noetisch-noematische Korrelation)** is the structure by which act and object-sense belong together. (心理事件是心灵生活中的事实性发生；意向活动—意向内容相关性则是活动与对象意义彼此归属的结构。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** this distinction transforms the early modern problem of idea and object. The question is no longer simply whether an idea represents an object correctly, but how an object is constituted as meaningful through intentional acts. (这一区分改造近代的观念与对象问题。问题不再只是观念是否正确表象对象，而是对象如何通过意向活动被构成为有意义之物。)  
  
### 6. Natural Attitude: The Problem of Unexamined World-Belief  
  
`Natural Attitude (自然态度; de: natürliche Einstellung)`  
**Definition:** the ordinary stance in which the world is taken for granted as simply existing. (世界被理所当然地视为简单存在的日常立场。)  
**Problem solved:** it names the unexamined background from which everyday and scientific thinking usually begin. (它命名日常思维和科学思维通常从中出发的未经审查背景。)  
**Why needed:** phenomenology must identify what must be suspended before experience can be described philosophically. (现象学必须识别在经验能够被哲学描述之前需要被悬置的东西。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing assumptions so basic that they usually remain unnoticed. (当分析那些过于基础以至通常不被注意的假设时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
In the natural attitude, one lives in the world without questioning its being. Tables, cities, institutions, bodies, other people, tools, and scientific facts are simply there. This attitude is not false. It is necessary for ordinary life. But it conceals the structures through which the world is given as meaningful.  
  
Phenomenology does not mock the natural attitude. It suspends it in order to see it.  
  
**Typical sentence:** The natural attitude is the everyday confidence that the world is simply there before reflection. (自然态度是反思之前对世界简单在那里这一点的日常确信。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Natural Attitude (自然态度; de: natürliche Einstellung)** differs from **Phenomenological Attitude (现象学态度; de: phänomenologische Einstellung)**. The first lives in the world as given; the second reflects on how the world is given. (自然态度生活于被给予的世界中；现象学态度反思世界如何被给予。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** the natural attitude becomes a target not of refutation but of methodological suspension. This is different from Cartesian doubt: the world is not denied, but bracketed. (自然态度成为方法性悬置的对象，而不是反驳的对象。这不同于笛卡尔式怀疑：世界不是被否认，而是被括号化。)  
  
### 7. Epoché: The Problem of Suspension  
  
`Epoché (悬置; el: ἐποχή; de: Epoché)`  
**Definition:** the suspension or bracketing of the natural attitude and its unexamined belief in the world. (对自然态度及其未经审查的世界信念进行悬置或括号化。)  
**Problem solved:** it frees inquiry from immediate commitment to the world’s taken-for-granted existence so that givenness itself can be described. (它使探究暂时摆脱对世界理所当然存在的直接承诺，从而描述给予性本身。)  
**Why needed:** without suspension, analysis remains trapped inside the assumptions it should examine. (如果没有悬置，分析就会被困在它本应审查的假设之中。)  
**How to use:** use it when a text brackets factual existence in order to analyze appearance, meaning, or constitution. (当文本把事实存在括号化，以分析显现、意义或构成时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
**Epoché** does not mean doubting that the world exists. It means suspending the automatic use of that belief. The question is not “does the table exist?” but “how is the table given as an object of perception, use, familiarity, distance, and possible verification?”  
  
This is why epoché is a method of access. It gives access not to another world, but to the structure of world-givenness.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Epoché does not abolish the world; it brackets the natural belief in the world in order to describe how the world is given. (悬置并不取消世界；它把对世界的自然信念括号化，以描述世界如何被给予。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Doubt (怀疑; la: dubitatio)** questions whether something is true; **Epoché (悬置; el: ἐποχή)** suspends commitment in order to examine givenness. (怀疑质疑某物是否为真；悬置暂停承诺，以便考察给予性。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** epoché transforms early modern method. Descartes used doubt to find certainty; Husserl uses suspension to disclose the structures of experience. (悬置改造近代方法。笛卡尔用怀疑寻找确定性；胡塞尔用悬置揭示经验结构。)  
  
### 8. Reduction: The Problem of Returning to Conditions of Givenness  
  
`Reduction (还原; la: reductio; de: Reduktion)`  
**Definition:** a methodological return from taken-for-granted objects to the structures through which they are given and constituted. (从被理所当然接受的对象返回到对象得以被给予和构成之结构的方法。)  
**Problem solved:** it redirects attention from the object as simply existing to the object as experienced, meant, and constituted. (它把注意力从作为简单存在的对象，转向作为被经验、被意指和被构成的对象。)  
**Why needed:** philosophical description must uncover the correlation between experiencing and experienced. (哲学描述必须揭示经验活动与被经验者之间的相关性。)  
**How to use:** use it when analysis moves from worldly objects to their mode of appearance or constitution. (当分析从世界中的对象转向其显现方式或构成方式时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Reduction does not reduce experience to something poorer. It returns to what is more fundamental for phenomenological analysis. It reduces not by impoverishing, but by redirecting.  
  
The **Transcendental Reduction (先验还原; de: transzendentale Reduktion)** moves from the natural world to the constitutive structures of consciousness. In Husserl, this is a return from the natural world to constitutive conditions.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Reduction returns from the world as assumed to the world as given. (还原从被预设的世界返回到被给予的世界。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Reduction (还原; de: Reduktion)** in phenomenology differs from **Reductionism (还原论; en: reductionism)**. Phenomenological reduction reveals structures of givenness; reductionism explains a phenomenon by reducing it to a lower-level cause. (现象学还原揭示给予性结构；还原论则把现象化约为低层原因。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** reduction continues Kant’s transcendental question but changes its method. Kant asks for conditions of possible experience; Husserl describes constitutive structures through reflective analysis of consciousness. (还原延续康德的先验问题，但改变其方法。康德追问可能经验条件；胡塞尔通过对意识的反思分析描述构成性结构。)  
  
### 9. Constitution: The Problem of How Objects Become Meaningful  
  
`Constitution (构成; de: Konstitution)`  
**Definition:** the process by which an object becomes meaningful and identifiable within intentional experience. (对象在意向经验中成为有意义且可识别之物的过程。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains objectivity as formed through structures of givenness, synthesis, horizon, and meaning. (它把客观性解释为通过给予性、综合、视域和意义结构形成的东西。)  
**Why needed:** objects are not merely received as finished units; they are given through profiles, acts, expectations, and horizons. (对象并非作为完成单位被简单接收；它们通过侧显、活动、期待和视域被给予。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing how something counts as a stable object across changing appearances. (当分析某物如何在变化显现中算作稳定对象时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Constitution does not mean that the subject arbitrarily creates objects out of nothing. It means that objectivity appears through structured intentional life. A cube is not given all at once. Only one side is visible now. Other sides are co-intended as possible appearances. The object is constituted as the same object across profiles.  
  
This is a powerful tool because it explains stability without returning to naive objectivism. Objectivity is not denied; it is described through the structures that make it experienceable.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Constitution names the process through which an object becomes identifiable as the same through changing modes of appearance. (构成命名一个对象通过变化的显现方式而成为可识别的同一对象的过程。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Creation (创造; la: creatio)** brings something into being; **Constitution (构成; de: Konstitution)** describes how something becomes meaningful as an object within experience. (创造使某物进入存在；构成描述某物如何在经验中作为对象而具有意义。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** constitution becomes a key alternative to both empiricist passivity and idealist construction. It describes how objectivity is experienced without reducing it to either brute fact or subjective invention. (构成成为经验论被动性与观念论建构之间的重要替代项。它描述客观性如何被经验，而不把它化约为赤裸事实或主观发明。)  
  
### 10. Givenness: The Problem of How Something Presents Itself  
  
`Givenness (给予性; de: Gegebenheit)`  
**Definition:** the mode in which something is presented or made available in experience. (某物在经验中被呈现或被提供的方式。)  
**Problem solved:** it allows philosophy to distinguish different ways in which objects, values, others, and meanings appear. (它使哲学能够区分对象、价值、他者与意义的不同显现方式。)  
**Why needed:** not all things are given in the same way. (并非所有东西都以同一种方式被给予。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing whether something is perceived, remembered, imagined, anticipated, judged, valued, or indirectly indicated. (当分析某物是被知觉、被记忆、被想象、被期待、被判断、被赋值，还是被间接指示时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Givenness is one of phenomenology’s most useful terms. A perceived object is given differently from a mathematical object. A pain is given differently from another person’s pain. A memory is given differently from current perception. A value is given differently from a color. An absence can also be given: the missing friend, the broken tool, the silence after a question.  
  
Phenomenology trains attention to these differences.  
  
**Typical sentence:** To describe givenness is to describe the way something becomes present or meaningful in experience. (描述给予性，就是描述某物在经验中变得在场或有意义的方式。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Presence (在场; de: Anwesenheit; fr: présence)** suggests appearing as there; **Givenness (给予性; de: Gegebenheit)** analyzes the mode by which that appearing occurs. (在场意味着作为在那里而显现；给予性分析这种显现发生的方式。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** givenness becomes a central battleground in later phenomenology, hermeneutics, and deconstruction. Derrida will question whether full presence is ever simply given, developing **Trace (痕迹; fr: trace)** and **Différance (延异; fr: différance)** as ways of destabilizing full presence.  
  
### 11. Horizon: The Problem of Background Meaning  
  
`Horizon (视域; de: Horizont)`  
**Definition:** the implicit background of possible meanings, appearances, expectations, and references surrounding any experience. (围绕任何经验的可能意义、显现、期待和指涉的隐含背景。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains why an object is never given in isolation. (它解释为什么对象从不孤立地被给予。)  
**Why needed:** every perception or meaning refers beyond itself to further possibilities. (每个知觉或意义都超出自身而指向进一步可能性。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing background, context, anticipation, implicit sense, or the open field of possible experience. (当分析背景、语境、期待、隐含意义或可能经验的开放场域时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
A horizon is not a subjective decoration added to objects. It belongs to how objects appear. A house is seen from one side, but it is experienced as having unseen sides. A word is heard in a sentence, but it carries linguistic and historical possibilities. A tool appears within a practical context. A person appears within a field of gestures, expectations, and social meanings.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Every object appears within a horizon of further possible appearances and meanings. (每个对象都在进一步可能显现与意义的视域中出现。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Object (对象; de: Gegenstand)** is what is thematically intended; **Horizon (视域; de: Horizont)** is the background field that lets the object have sense. (对象是被主题化意指之物；视域是使对象具有意义的背景场域。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** horizon becomes central for hermeneutics. Gadamer will later develop understanding through historical horizons and the **Fusion of Horizons (视域融合; de: Horizontverschmelzung)**, a central name for historically mediated understanding.  
  
### 12. Lifeworld: The Problem of the Pre-Theoretical World  
  
`Lifeworld (生活世界; de: Lebenswelt)`  
**Definition:** the pre-theoretical, everyday world of lived meaning that underlies scientific and theoretical abstraction. (支撑科学和理论抽象的前理论的、日常的、被生活的意义世界。)  
**Problem solved:** it reveals the forgotten ground of objective science and formal theory. (它揭示客观科学与形式理论被遗忘的根据。)  
**Why needed:** science abstracts from the world we already live in, but it can forget that dependence. (科学从我们已经生活其中的世界中抽象出来，但它可能遗忘这种依赖。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing everyday meaning, practical familiarity, shared worldhood, or the background of scientific objectification. (当分析日常意义、实践熟悉性、共享世界性或科学客体化的背景时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
The lifeworld is not a primitive error to be overcome by science. It is the ground from which scientific abstraction becomes possible. Measuring, calculating, theorizing, and objectifying all presuppose a world already meaningful in practice.  
  
This concept is one of phenomenology’s strongest answers to modern scientific reduction. The mathematical world of science is powerful, but it is abstracted from a lived world of bodies, tools, others, language, practice, and expectation.  
  
**Typical sentence:** The lifeworld is the pre-theoretical world that science presupposes but often forgets. (生活世界是科学所预设但常常遗忘的前理论世界。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Objective World of Science (科学客观世界; en: objective world of science)** is abstract, measurable, and formalized; **Lifeworld (生活世界; de: Lebenswelt)** is lived, practical, historical, and pre-theoretical. (科学客观世界是抽象的、可度量的和形式化的；生活世界则是被生活的、实践的、历史的和前理论的。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** lifeworld reopens the problem created by early modern mechanism and primary qualities. It asks what is lost when the world of lived experience is subordinated to the mathematically objectified world. (生活世界重新打开近代机械论和第一性质理论所制造的问题。它追问：当被生活的经验世界从属于数学化客体世界时，什么被丢失了？)  
  
### 13. Perception: The Problem of Embodied Access  
  
`Perception (知觉; la: perceptio; fr: perception; de: Wahrnehmung)`  
**Definition:** the embodied and situated way in which things are directly encountered as meaningful. (事物作为有意义之物被直接遭遇的具身且处境化方式。)  
**Problem solved:** it challenges the model of perception as passive reception of sensory data. (它挑战把知觉视为感官材料被动接受的模型。)  
**Why needed:** the world is not first given as neutral data; it is encountered through bodily orientation, movement, interest, and practical possibility. (世界并非首先作为中立材料被给予；它通过身体取向、运动、兴趣和实践可能性被遭遇。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing bodily orientation, spatiality, practical engagement, or direct world-contact. (当分析身体取向、空间性、实践牵连或同世界的直接接触时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Phenomenological perception is not the assembly of raw sensations into an object. It is an active, embodied, world-involved access. One does not first receive color patches and then infer a cup. The cup is encountered as graspable, usable, near, fragile, empty, mine, or out of reach.  
  
This is especially important in Merleau-Ponty’s development of phenomenology. The body is not one object among others; it is the condition of having a world.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Perception is not the reception of neutral data but embodied access to a meaningful world. (知觉不是中立材料的接收，而是对有意义世界的具身通达。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Sensation (感觉; la: sensatio)** can be treated as isolated sensory content; **Perception (知觉; de: Wahrnehmung)** is structured encounter with objects in a world. (感觉可以被处理为孤立感官内容；知觉则是同世界中对象的结构化遭遇。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** phenomenological perception resists early modern empiricism and scientific objectivism. It prepares later philosophy of embodiment, affect, skill, habit, and ecological perception. (现象学知觉反抗近代经验论和科学客体主义，并为后来的具身性、情感、技能、习惯和生态知觉哲学做准备。)  
  
### 14. Embodiment: The Problem of the Body as Subject  
  
`Embodiment (具身性; de: Leiblichkeit; fr: incarnation/corporéité)`  
**Definition:** the structure by which subjectivity exists through a lived body rather than as a detached mind. (主体性通过被生活的身体而存在，而不是作为脱离身体的心灵而存在的结构。)  
**Problem solved:** it overcomes the split between mind as inner subject and body as external object. (它克服心灵作为内部主体与身体作为外部对象之间的分裂。)  
**Why needed:** perception, action, orientation, habit, and world-access all depend on the lived body. (知觉、行动、取向、习惯和世界通达都依赖被生活的身体。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing bodily subjectivity, skill, habit, affect, spatial orientation, or vulnerability. (当分析身体主体性、技能、习惯、情感、空间取向或脆弱性时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Phenomenology distinguishes the lived body from the body as object.  
  
**Lived Body (被生活的身体; de: Leib)** is the body from which one perceives, acts, suffers, reaches, moves, and inhabits the world. (Leib 是人借以知觉、行动、受苦、伸手、运动并居住于世界中的身体。)  
  
**Objective Body (客观身体; de: Körper)** is the body as observed, measured, anatomized, or treated as a physical thing. (Körper 是被观察、测量、解剖或作为物理事物处理的身体。)  
  
This distinction is one of the most important phenomenological tools. A hand touching another hand is both touching and touchable. The body is not merely an object I possess; it is the medium of my being-in-the-world.  
  
**Typical sentence:** The lived body is not an object added to consciousness; it is the way consciousness has a world. (被生活的身体不是附加给意识的对象，而是意识拥有世界的方式。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Leib (被生活的身体; de: Leib)** differs from **Körper (客观身体; de: Körper)**. Leib is lived from within; Körper is observed from without. (Leib 是从内部被生活的身体；Körper 是从外部被观察的身体。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** embodiment transforms the modern subject. The subject is no longer a pure thinking point, but a bodily, affective, situated being. This prepares existentialism, feminist phenomenology, disability theory, affect theory, and contemporary cognitive science. (具身性改造现代主体。主体不再是纯粹思维点，而是身体性的、情感性的、处境化的存在。)  
  
### 15. Temporality: The Problem of Lived Time  
  
`Temporality (时间性; de: Zeitlichkeit; fr: temporalité)`  
**Definition:** the lived structure of time through retention, presence, anticipation, memory, and expectation. (通过保持、当前、预期、记忆和期待构成的被生活的时间结构。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains experience as flowing and internally structured rather than as a sequence of isolated now-points. (它把经验解释为流动且内部结构化的东西，而不是孤立“现在点”的序列。)  
**Why needed:** consciousness is not static; every experience includes retention of what has just passed and anticipation of what is coming. (意识不是静态的；每个经验都包含对刚刚过去之物的保持与对即将到来之物的预期。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing memory, expectation, rhythm, continuity, anticipation, or the flow of experience. (当分析记忆、期待、节奏、连续性、预期或经验流时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
A melody shows why temporality matters. One does not hear isolated notes and then add them together. Each note is heard with retention of previous notes and anticipation of coming notes. Meaning unfolds temporally.  
  
This means that consciousness is internally temporal. Even perception has a temporal structure. The object appears across profiles, moments, and expectations.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Lived time is not a chain of isolated instants; it is the structured flow through which meaning endures and changes. (被生活的时间不是孤立瞬间的链条，而是意义得以持续和变化的结构化流动。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Objective Time (客观时间; de: objektive Zeit)** is measured by clocks; **Lived Temporality (被生活的时间性; de: gelebte Zeitlichkeit)** is experienced as retention, anticipation, delay, urgency, boredom, rhythm, or memory. (客观时间由钟表度量；被生活的时间性则作为保持、预期、延迟、紧迫、无聊、节奏或记忆被经验。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** phenomenological temporality prepares Heidegger’s existential analysis of time. Heidegger’s **Dasein (此在; de: Dasein)** and temporality become central to his rethinking of Being.  
  
### 16. Intersubjectivity: The Problem of Other Minds and Shared World  
  
`Intersubjectivity (主体间性; de: Intersubjektivität)`  
**Definition:** the structure through which subjects encounter one another and share a common world. (主体彼此遭遇并共享一个共同世界的结构。)  
**Problem solved:** it addresses how other subjects are given as subjects rather than as mere objects. (它处理他者如何作为主体而非单纯对象被给予。)  
**Why needed:** objectivity, language, social meaning, and worldhood require more than isolated consciousness. (客观性、语言、社会意义和世界性需要的不只是孤立意识。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing empathy, recognition, other minds, social experience, or shared meaning. (当分析移情、承认、他心、社会经验或共享意义时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Phenomenology cannot remain inside solitary consciousness. The world is experienced as shared. Other people are not usually inferred as hidden minds behind bodies. They appear directly through gesture, expression, voice, posture, action, and responsiveness.  
  
This is not the same as Hegelian recognition, though the problems are related. Hegel emphasizes struggle and social status. Phenomenology emphasizes how the other is given in experience and how a shared world becomes possible.  
  
**Typical sentence:** The other is not first a body plus an inference; the other is given as another subject within a shared world. (他者并非首先是身体加推论；他者是在共享世界中作为另一个主体被给予。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Intersubjectivity (主体间性; de: Intersubjektivität)** differs from **Solipsism (唯我论; la: solus ipse)**. Intersubjectivity describes the shared field in which subjectivity is never simply isolated. (主体间性不同于唯我论；它描述主体性从不只是孤立的共享场域。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** intersubjectivity links phenomenology with hermeneutics, social theory, recognition theory, ethics, and political philosophy. (主体间性把现象学同解释学、社会理论、承认理论、伦理学和政治哲学连接起来。)  
  
### 17. World: The Problem of Meaningful Context  
  
`World (世界; de: Welt; fr: monde)`  
**Definition:** not merely the totality of objects, but the meaningful context in which objects, actions, others, and possibilities appear. (不只是对象总和，而是对象、行动、他者与可能性在其中显现的意义语境。)  
**Problem solved:** it prevents experience from being reduced to isolated subject-object relations. (它防止经验被化约为孤立的主体—客体关系。)  
**Why needed:** every object appears within a practical, historical, bodily, and social world. (每个对象都在实践的、历史的、身体的和社会的世界中显现。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing contextual meaning, practical involvement, worldhood, or the background of objectivity. (当分析语境意义、实践牵连、世界性或客观性的背景时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Phenomenology uses **World** in a technical sense. The world is not merely a container holding objects. It is the open context within which objects have sense. A hammer appears as useful within a workshop. A street appears as walkable or dangerous. A sentence appears within a language. A person appears within a shared social world.  
  
This concept leads directly toward Heidegger’s **Being-in-the-world (在世存在; de: In-der-Welt-sein)**. Heidegger’s **Dasein** is not a detached subject but being-in-the-world.  
  
**Typical sentence:** World is the meaningful context within which objects can appear as usable, threatening, familiar, distant, valuable, or strange. (世界是对象得以作为可用的、威胁性的、熟悉的、遥远的、有价值的或陌生的东西而显现的意义语境。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **World (世界; de: Welt)** differs from **Universe (宇宙; la: universum)**. Universe suggests the totality of things; world names the meaningful horizon of experience and action. (宇宙暗示事物总和；世界命名经验与行动的意义地平线。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** world becomes a central alternative to the subject-object model. Heidegger, hermeneutics, existentialism, and later social ontology all inherit this term. (世界成为主体—客体模型的重要替代项。海德格尔、解释学、存在主义和后来的社会本体论都继承了这一术语。)  
  
### 18. Description: The Problem of Philosophical Style  
  
`Description (描述; la: descriptio; de: Beschreibung)`  
**Definition:** the disciplined articulation of how phenomena are given. (对现象如何被给予的有规训阐明。)  
**Problem solved:** it provides a philosophical method that does not begin by deduction, causal explanation, or suspicion. (它提供一种不以演绎、因果解释或怀疑为起点的哲学方法。)  
**Why needed:** phenomena can be distorted if theory explains them before seeing how they appear. (如果理论在看清现象如何显现之前就解释它们，现象可能被扭曲。)  
**How to use:** use it when the task is to clarify experience rather than explain it away. (当任务是澄清经验而不是把它解释掉时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Phenomenological description is not casual reporting. It requires discipline. It brackets assumptions, attends to modes of givenness, distinguishes act and object, traces horizons, and clarifies lived structures.  
  
This also explains the style of phenomenological writing. It often proceeds slowly, with examples: seeing a cube, hearing a melody, touching one’s hand, using a tool, encountering another person. These examples are not decorative; they are methodological instruments.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Description is not pre-theoretical naivety; it is the disciplined effort to let the structure of appearing show itself. (描述不是前理论的天真，而是让显现结构自身显现出来的有规训努力。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Description (描述; de: Beschreibung)** differs from **Explanation (解释/说明; de: Erklärung)**. Explanation seeks causes; description clarifies structures of appearance. (说明寻求原因；描述澄清显现结构。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** phenomenological description becomes a major alternative to both analytic formalization and genealogical suspicion. It insists that before concepts are explained away, their experiential basis must be described. (现象学描述成为分析哲学形式化与谱系学怀疑之外的重要替代项。它坚持在概念被解释掉之前，必须描述其经验基础。)  
  
### 19. The Tool-Map of Phenomenology  
  
Use phenomenological vocabulary diagnostically. The core question is usually not “What causes this?” but “How is this given?”  
  
**If the text asks how consciousness is related to objects**, look for **Intentionality (意向性; de: Intentionalität)**, **Noesis (意向活动; el: νόησις)**, and **Noema (意向内容; el: νόημα)**.  
(如果文本追问意识如何同对象发生关系，应寻找意向性、意向活动和意向内容问题。)  
  
**If the text suspends ordinary belief in the world**, look for **Natural Attitude (自然态度; de: natürliche Einstellung)**, **Epoché (悬置; el: ἐποχή)**, and **Reduction (还原; de: Reduktion)**.  
(如果文本悬置对世界的日常信念，应寻找自然态度、悬置和还原问题。)  
  
**If the text asks how an object becomes meaningful**, look for **Constitution (构成; de: Konstitution)**, **Givenness (给予性; de: Gegebenheit)**, and **Horizon (视域; de: Horizont)**.  
(如果文本追问对象如何成为有意义之物，应寻找构成、给予性和视域问题。)  
  
**If the text criticizes scientific abstraction**, look for **Lifeworld (生活世界; de: Lebenswelt)** and **World (世界; de: Welt)**.  
(如果文本批判科学抽象，应寻找生活世界与世界问题。)  
  
**If the text analyzes bodily access to the world**, look for **Perception (知觉; de: Wahrnehmung)**, **Embodiment (具身性; de: Leiblichkeit)**, **Lived Body (被生活的身体; de: Leib)**, and **Objective Body (客观身体; de: Körper)**.  
(如果文本分析身体对世界的通达，应寻找知觉、具身性、被生活的身体与客观身体问题。)  
  
**If the text analyzes time as experienced**, look for **Temporality (时间性; de: Zeitlichkeit)**, **Retention (保持; de: Retention)**, and **Anticipation/Protention (预期; de: Protention)**.  
(如果文本分析被经验的时间，应寻找时间性、保持和预期问题。)  
  
**If the text asks how others and shared worlds appear**, look for **Intersubjectivity (主体间性; de: Intersubjektivität)** and **Empathy (移情; de: Einfühlung)**.  
(如果文本追问他者与共享世界如何显现，应寻找主体间性与移情问题。)  
  
### 20. The Genealogical Point of Part 7  
  
Phenomenology transforms modern philosophy by shifting attention from secure representation, historical production, or conceptual system to the structures of lived givenness. Early modern philosophy asked how the subject represents the object. Kant asked what conditions make experience possible. German Idealism made those conditions dynamic and historical. Marx and Nietzsche asked what social forces and values produce concepts. Phenomenology asks how any object, world, value, body, or other person is first given as meaningful in experience.  
  
The guiding thesis is:  
  
**Phenomenological language turns philosophy toward givenness: to understand a thing is to describe how it appears, is intended, is constituted, and belongs to a lived world.**  
(现象学语言把哲学转向给予性：理解一个事物，就是描述它如何显现、被意指、被构成，并归属于一个被生活的世界。)  
  
This grammar will shape the next stages of continental philosophy. Heidegger transforms phenomenology into an existential ontology of **Dasein (此在; de: Dasein)** and **Being-in-the-world (在世存在; de: In-der-Welt-sein)**. Merleau-Ponty deepens the analysis of embodiment and perception. Sartre turns intentionality toward freedom, nothingness, and bad faith. Hermeneutics transforms horizon into historical understanding. Derrida questions whether givenness can ever be pure presence. Foucault does not adopt Husserlian phenomenology as his method, but his historical analysis of knowledge still inherits the post-Kantian and post-phenomenological problem of the conditions under which something can appear, count, and be known.  
  
The phenomenological question remains one of the most useful tools for reading philosophy:  
  
**How is this object, value, body, other, or world given before it is explained?**  
(这个对象、价值、身体、他者或世界，在被解释之前是如何被给予的？)  
  
## Part 8. Heidegger: Dasein, Being, Time  
  
This chapter explains Heidegger’s transformation of phenomenology into existential ontology. Husserlian phenomenology had asked how objects are given to consciousness. Heidegger radicalizes the question: before any subject represents an object, there is already a way of being in which beings matter, show up, withdraw, threaten, invite use, and become intelligible. The central question is therefore not first **how consciousness knows objects**, but **what it means for beings to be**. (核心问题不是意识如何认识对象，而是存在者之“存在”意味着什么。)  
  
The central vocabulary is **Dasein**, **Being**, **beings**, **ontological difference**, **Being-in-the-world**, **world**, **care**, **thrownness**, **projection**, **fallenness**, **authenticity**, **being-toward-death**, **temporality**, **disclosure**, **truth as unconcealment**, **clearing**, **Ereignis**, and **Gestell**. **Dasein** is Heidegger’s term for human existence, while the difference between **Sein** and **Seiendes** is Heidegger’s **ontological difference**. Heidegger also technicalizes ordinary words such as **world**, **truth**, and **being**.  
  
The operational function of this chapter is exact: use Heideggerian vocabulary when the problem is **not an object inside consciousness**, but the more basic structure through which beings become intelligible as beings. (当问题不是意识中的对象，而是存在者作为存在者而变得可理解的更基本结构时，应使用海德格尔式词汇。)  
  
### 1. The Problem-Situation: From Consciousness to Being  
  
Phenomenology had already moved beyond the early modern model of an inner subject representing an outer object. Heidegger goes further. He argues that even phenomenology can remain too centered on consciousness if it does not ask about the being of the one who asks the question.  
  
The question becomes:  
  
**What kind of being must the questioner be in order to ask about Being at all?**  
(为了能够追问存在，提问者本身必须是一种什么样的存在者？)  
  
This is why Heidegger begins with **Dasein (此在; de: Dasein)**. Dasein is not “the human being” as a biological species, psychological subject, rational animal, or Cartesian ego. It names the being for whom its own being is an issue.  
  
This changes the grammar of philosophy.  
  
Not: **subject represents object**.  
(不是：主体表象客体。)  
  
Not even only: **consciousness intends object**.  
(甚至不只是：意识意向对象。)  
  
But: **Dasein exists as being-in-the-world and already understands Being in a pre-theoretical way**.  
(而是：此在作为在世存在而存在，并且已经以前理论方式理解存在。)  
  
**Typical sentence:** The question of Being must begin with the being for whom Being is already at issue. (存在问题必须从这样一种存在者开始：对它而言，存在已经成问题。)  
  
### 2. Dasein: The Problem of the Being That Asks about Being  
  
`Dasein (此在; de: Dasein/Da-sein)`  
**Definition:** the being that exists in such a way that its own being is an issue for it. (这样一种存在者：它以自身存在对其自身成问题的方式存在。)  
**Problem solved:** it avoids treating the human being as a detached subject, biological object, or rational substance. (它避免把人理解为脱离世界的主体、生物学对象或理性实体。)  
**Why needed:** the question of Being must be approached through the being that already has some pre-theoretical understanding of Being. (存在问题必须通过一种已经具有前理论存在理解的存在者来进入。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing human existence as situated, finite, practical, temporal, and world-involved. (当分析人类存在作为处境化的、有限的、实践的、时间性的和牵连于世界的存在时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
**Dasein** literally means “being-there.” The *Da* is not merely a location in physical space. It names the opened “there” in which beings can show up. Dasein is the site or clearing in which a world is disclosed.  
  
This is why translating Dasein simply as “human being” is too weak. Heidegger does not begin with a human animal and add consciousness. He begins with an existential structure: Dasein is the being that understands, cares, projects, is thrown, falls, dies, and asks about Being.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Dasein is not a subject enclosed in itself; it is the open “there” in which a world is disclosed. (此在不是封闭于自身内部的主体，而是世界在其中被开显的开放之“此”。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Dasein (此在; de: Dasein)** differs from **Subject (主体; la: subiectum; de: Subjekt)**. The subject is often treated as a knowing center opposed to objects; Dasein is always already being-in-the-world. (主体常被视为同客体相对的认识中心；此在则总是已经在世界之中存在。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** Dasein transforms the modern subject. The Cartesian **Cogito (我思; la: cogito)** begins from thinking self-certainty; Dasein begins from finite, practical, world-involved existence. (此在改造现代主体。笛卡尔的我思从思维的自我确定性出发；此在从有限的、实践的、牵连于世界的存在出发。)  
  
### 3. Being and Beings: The Problem of Ontological Difference  
  
`Being (存在; el: εἶναι/τὸ ὄν; de: Sein)`  
**Definition:** not an entity, but the meaning or disclosedness of entities as beings. (不是一个存在者，而是存在者作为存在者的意义或开显性。)  
**Problem solved:** it prevents philosophy from confusing Being with the highest or most general being. (它防止哲学把存在同最高或最普遍的存在者混淆。)  
**Why needed:** metaphysics often studies beings while forgetting the question of Being itself. (形而上学常研究存在者，却遗忘存在本身的问题。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing the condition under which beings can appear as beings. (当分析存在者何以能够作为存在者显现的条件时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
`Beings (存在者; el: τὰ ὄντα; de: Seiendes)`  
**Definition:** entities, things, persons, tools, objects, events, institutions, or anything that is. (实体、事物、人、工具、对象、事件、制度，或任何存在着的东西。)  
**Problem solved:** it marks the domain of what exists without confusing it with Being itself. (它标明存在着的东西之领域，同时不把它同存在本身混淆。)  
**Why needed:** ontology must distinguish entities from the meaning of their being. (存在论必须区分存在者与其存在之意义。)  
**How to use:** use it when referring to entities rather than the disclosedness or meaning of Being. (当指称存在者而非存在的开显性或意义时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
The distinction between **Being** and **beings** is Heidegger’s **Ontological Difference (存在论差异; de: ontologische Differenz)**. It is the hinge of his philosophy. The problem is not that philosophers ignored entities. They studied substances, causes, minds, bodies, God, nature, values, and objects. The problem is that they often treated Being as if it were another being, perhaps the highest being, most universal property, or most abstract concept.  
  
For Heidegger, this misses the question. Being is not a thing. It is that in virtue of which beings are intelligible as beings.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Being is not one being among others; it is that through which beings are disclosed as beings. (存在不是诸存在者中的一个存在者，而是存在者借以作为存在者被开显的东西。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Ontic (存在者层面的; de: ontisch)** concerns beings and facts about beings; **Ontological (存在论的; de: ontologisch)** concerns the Being of beings. (Ontic 关涉存在者以及关于存在者的事实；ontological 关涉存在者之存在。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** Heidegger reopens the Greek question of **Being / What-is (存在/所是者; el: τὸ εἶναι / τὸ ὄν)** against the Latin metaphysical tendency to convert Being into substance, essence, ground, or highest being. (海德格尔反对拉丁形而上学把存在转化为实体、本质、根据或最高存在者的倾向，重新打开希腊的存在问题。)  
  
### 4. Fundamental Ontology: The Problem of the Meaning of Being  
  
`Fundamental Ontology (基础存在论; de: Fundamentalontologie)`  
**Definition:** the inquiry into the meaning of Being through the existential analysis of Dasein. (通过对此在的存在论分析来探究存在意义的工作。)  
**Problem solved:** it gives ontology a starting point in the being that already understands Being. (它使存在论从已经理解存在的存在者出发。)  
**Why needed:** Being cannot be approached as an object among objects; it must be approached through Dasein’s disclosed existence. (存在不能作为诸对象中的对象来进入；它必须通过此在被开显的生存来进入。)  
**How to use:** use it when the analysis of human existence is being used as a route to the question of Being. (当对人类存在的分析被用作进入存在问题的路径时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Fundamental ontology is not anthropology. Heidegger is not primarily asking what humans are biologically, psychologically, or culturally. He analyzes Dasein because Dasein is the being that already has an understanding of Being, however vague.  
  
This gives the analysis of existence a special status. It is not merely one regional study. It opens the access to ontology.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Fundamental ontology analyzes Dasein not as an object of human science, but as the site where the meaning of Being is disclosed. (基础存在论分析此在，并不是把它作为人类科学的对象，而是作为存在意义被开显的位置。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Anthropology (人类学; de: Anthropologie)** studies the human being as a kind of entity; **Fundamental Ontology (基础存在论; de: Fundamentalontologie)** studies Dasein as access to the question of Being. (人类学把人作为一种存在者来研究；基础存在论把此在作为进入存在问题的通道来研究。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** this move displaces both Cartesian subjectivity and Kantian transcendental subjectivity. The condition of intelligibility is no longer a formal subject alone, but finite existence in a world. (这一转变移置了笛卡尔式主体性与康德式先验主体性。可理解性的条件不再只是形式主体，而是在世界中的有限生存。)  
  
### 5. Being-in-the-World: The Problem of the False Inner/Outer Split  
  
`Being-in-the-world (在世存在; de: In-der-Welt-sein)`  
**Definition:** the basic structure of Dasein as always already involved in a meaningful world. (此在总是已经牵连于有意义世界之中的基本结构。)  
**Problem solved:** it overcomes the split between inner subject and outer world. (它克服内部主体与外部世界之间的分裂。)  
**Why needed:** Dasein does not first exist inside itself and then reach out to a world; it is world-involved from the beginning. (此在并非先存在于自身内部，然后才通向世界；它从一开始就是牵连于世界的。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing existence as practical, situated, relational, and already immersed in meaning. (当分析存在作为实践的、处境化的、关系性的并已经沉浸于意义之中时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
**Being-in-the-world** is a single structure, not three separate pieces: being, in, world. The “in” is not spatial containment, as water is in a glass. It is involvement, familiarity, dwelling, concern, and practical orientation.  
  
This is why Heidegger rejects the traditional epistemological problem of how an inner subject reaches an external object. That problem is derivative. Dasein already inhabits a meaningful world before it theorizes objects.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Dasein does not first stand inside consciousness and then infer a world; Dasein exists as being-in-the-world. (此在并非先站在意识内部然后推论出世界；此在作为在世存在而存在。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Being-in-the-world (在世存在; de: In-der-Welt-sein)** differs from **Subject-Object Relation (主体—客体关系; de: Subjekt-Objekt-Beziehung)**. The latter treats subject and object as separable poles; the former names the prior unity of practical involvement. (主体—客体关系把主体与客体视为可分离的两极；在世存在命名实践牵连的先行统一性。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** Heidegger radicalizes phenomenology’s concept of **World (世界; de: Welt)**. World is not the totality of objects, but the meaningful context in which beings can show up. (海德格尔激进化现象学的世界概念。世界不是对象总和，而是存在者得以显现的意义语境。)  
  
### 6. World: The Problem of Significance  
  
`World (世界; de: Welt)`  
**Definition:** the meaningful network of relations, references, practices, and possibilities within which beings are encountered. (存在者在其中被遭遇的由关系、指涉、实践和可能性构成的意义网络。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains why things appear first as meaningful rather than as neutral objects. (它解释为什么事物首先作为有意义之物而非中立对象显现。)  
**Why needed:** Dasein encounters tools, others, tasks, dangers, and possibilities within a world of significance. (此在在意义世界中遭遇工具、他者、任务、危险和可能性。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing background meaning, practical context, familiarity, or the referential whole in which things matter. (当分析背景意义、实践语境、熟悉性或事物在其中有意义的指涉整体时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Heidegger’s **world** is not the same as the physical universe. A laboratory, kitchen, courtroom, battlefield, temple, classroom, and home are worlds in the sense that beings appear there through roles, practices, expectations, and possibilities.  
  
Worldhood is the condition for encountering things as meaningful. A hammer appears as hammer only within a practical nexus: nails, wood, building, repairing, hand, task, workshop, and purpose.  
  
**Typical sentence:** World is the referential whole within which beings show up as usable, threatening, familiar, or significant. (世界是存在者得以作为可用的、威胁性的、熟悉的或有意义的东西而显现的指涉整体。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **World (世界; de: Welt)** differs from **Universe (宇宙; la: universum)**. Universe names the totality of entities; world names the structure of significance within which entities matter. (宇宙命名存在者总和；世界命名存在者在其中有意义的意义结构。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** the world concept transforms phenomenological **Horizon (视域; de: Horizont)** into an existential structure. It is not just a background of possible appearances, but the practical field in which Dasein exists. (世界概念把现象学视域转化为存在论结构。它不只是可能显现的背景，而是此在生存其中的实践场域。)  
  
### 7. Readiness-to-Hand: The Problem of Practical Encounter  
  
`Ready-to-Hand (上手状态; de: Zuhandenheit)`  
**Definition:** the mode in which equipment is encountered in use, as practically available rather than theoretically observed. (器具在使用中作为实践上可用之物而非理论观察对象被遭遇的方式。)  
**Problem solved:** it shows that practical involvement is more basic than detached observation. (它显示实践牵连比脱离式观察更基本。)  
**Why needed:** Dasein usually encounters things through use, task, and concern, not first through neutral perception. (此在通常通过使用、任务和操劳遭遇事物，而不是首先通过中立知觉。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing tools, equipment, practical familiarity, skill, or absorbed activity. (当分析工具、器具、实践熟悉性、技能或沉浸式活动时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
**Ready-to-hand** is one of Heidegger’s most useful concepts. A hammer in use is not first a physical object with properties. It is something for hammering. Its being is disclosed through practical use. The worker does not stare at it as a neutral object; the worker is absorbed in the task.  
  
This means that theoretical observation is not the basic way beings show up. It is derivative from practical involvement.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Equipment first appears not as an object with properties, but as something for doing something. (器具首先并不作为具有属性的对象显现，而是作为用来做某事的东西显现。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Ready-to-Hand (上手状态; de: Zuhandenheit)** contrasts with **Present-at-Hand (现成在手状态; de: Vorhandenheit)**. The ready-to-hand is encountered in use; the present-at-hand is observed as a detached object. (上手状态是在使用中被遭遇；现成在手状态则是作为脱离式对象被观察。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** Heidegger reverses the priority of theory. Instead of treating practical use as applied theoretical knowledge, he treats theoretical observation as a modification of prior practical involvement. (海德格尔反转理论的优先性。他不把实践使用视为理论知识的应用，而把理论观察视为先行实践牵连的一种变形。)  
  
### 8. Presence-at-Hand: The Problem of Theoretical Objectification  
  
`Present-at-Hand (现成在手状态; de: Vorhandenheit)`  
**Definition:** the mode in which something is encountered as a detached object with properties. (某物作为具有属性的脱离式对象被遭遇的方式。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains the ontological mode presupposed by theoretical observation and science. (它解释理论观察和科学所预设的存在论方式。)  
**Why needed:** not all encounter with beings is practical use; beings can also be thematized, measured, and observed. (并非所有存在者遭遇都是实践使用；存在者也可以被主题化、测量和观察。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing scientific objectification, detached perception, measurement, or theoretical attitude. (当分析科学客体化、脱离式知觉、测量或理论态度时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Presence-at-hand is not false. It is one possible mode of disclosure. The problem arises when philosophy treats it as the primary or only mode of being. If all beings are understood as present-at-hand objects, the practical, existential, and worlded character of Dasein’s life is obscured.  
  
A broken hammer often reveals this shift. When the hammer works, it withdraws into use. When it breaks, it becomes conspicuous as an object. The theoretical attitude often arises from breakdown in practical involvement.  
  
**Typical sentence:** The present-at-hand appears when a being is detached from practical involvement and treated as an object of observation. (当存在者脱离实践牵连并被作为观察对象处理时，现成在手状态就出现了。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Present-at-Hand (现成在手状态; de: Vorhandenheit)** is not more real than **Ready-to-Hand (上手状态; de: Zuhandenheit)**. It is a different mode of disclosure. (现成在手状态并不比上手状态更真实；它只是不同的开显方式。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** this distinction critiques early modern and scientific objectivism. It asks what is lost when beings are understood only as objects with measurable properties. (这一区分批判近代和科学客体主义。它追问：当存在者只被理解为具有可度量属性的对象时，什么被丢失了？)  
  
### 9. Care: The Problem of Dasein’s Basic Structure  
  
`Care (操心/牵挂; de: Sorge)`  
**Definition:** the basic structure of Dasein as concerned, involved, projected, thrown, and responsible for its own being. (此在作为有所关切、牵连、筹划、被抛并对自身存在有所担当的基本结构。)  
**Problem solved:** it unifies Dasein’s existence as practical, affective, temporal, and world-involved. (它把此在的生存统一为实践的、情感的、时间性的和牵连于世界的。)  
**Why needed:** Dasein is not a neutral observer; it is a being for whom things matter. (此在不是中立观察者；它是一种事物对其有关系、有分量的存在者。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing concern, involvement, responsibility, projection, anxiety, or the meaningfulness of existence. (当分析关切、牵连、责任、筹划、焦虑或生存意义时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
**Care** does not mean simply emotional worry. It names the structure through which Dasein is always ahead of itself, already in a world, and involved with beings. Dasein cares because its own being is at stake.  
  
This concept is the center of *Being and Time*. It gathers thrownness, projection, fallenness, temporality, and being-in-the-world into one existential structure.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Care means that Dasein’s being is never indifferent to itself. (操心意味着此在的存在对其自身从不无关紧要。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Care (操心; de: Sorge)** differs from **Cognition (认识; de: Erkenntnis)**. Cognition is one mode of relation to beings; care is the more basic structure in which beings matter at all. (认识是同存在者发生关系的一种方式；操心则是存在者之所以有意义的更基本结构。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** care transforms the modern subject from a knowing center into an existential being whose life is structured by concern, finitude, and possibility. (操心把现代主体从认识中心转化为由关切、有限性和可能性结构化的生存存在者。)  
  
### 10. Thrownness: The Problem of Facticity  
  
`Thrownness (被抛性; de: Geworfenheit)`  
**Definition:** Dasein’s condition of already finding itself in a world, situation, history, body, language, and set of possibilities not chosen by itself. (此在已经发现自身处于并非由自身选择的世界、处境、历史、身体、语言和可能性中的状态。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains the factical givenness of existence. (它解释生存的事实性给予状态。)  
**Why needed:** freedom is never exercised from nowhere; it begins from conditions already given. (自由从不在无处之地被行使；它从已经被给予的条件中开始。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing finitude, situation, facticity, inherited possibilities, or the non-chosen conditions of existence. (当分析有限性、处境、事实性、继承的可能性或非选择的生存条件时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Thrownness prevents existential analysis from becoming pure voluntarism. Dasein projects possibilities, but it does not invent itself from nothing. It is born into a world, language, history, body, social order, and mortality.  
  
This makes Heidegger’s account of freedom more precise. Freedom is not abstract self-creation. It is projection from thrown conditions.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Dasein is free only as thrown; it projects itself from conditions it did not choose. (此在只有作为被抛者才是自由的；它从并非由自己选择的条件中筹划自身。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Thrownness (被抛性; de: Geworfenheit)** contrasts with **Self-Origination (自我起源; en: self-origination)**. Dasein is not the origin of all its conditions. (被抛性与自我起源相对。此在并非其所有条件的起源。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** thrownness becomes a key alternative to both Cartesian self-certainty and Sartrean voluntarism. It also prepares later analyses of historical situatedness, embodiment, and social condition. (被抛性成为笛卡尔式自我确定性与萨特式意志主义之外的重要替代项，并为后来的历史处境性、具身性和社会条件分析做准备。)  
  
### 11. Projection: The Problem of Possibility  
  
`Projection (投射/筹划; de: Entwurf)`  
**Definition:** Dasein’s opening of itself toward possibilities of being. (此在朝向自身存在可能性的开启。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains Dasein as possibility rather than fixed essence. (它把此在解释为可能性，而非固定本质。)  
**Why needed:** Dasein is not merely what it factually is; it exists by understanding itself in terms of possibilities. (此在不只是事实上的所是；它通过以可能性理解自身而存在。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing self-understanding, future orientation, choice, possibility, or existential becoming. (当分析自我理解、未来取向、选择、可能性或生存生成时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Projection does not mean imagining fantasies. It is the existential structure by which Dasein lives ahead of itself. Dasein is always already oriented toward possibilities: to work, flee, speak, remain silent, become, refuse, inherit, or transform.  
  
Projection and thrownness belong together. Dasein is thrown into conditions, but projects possibilities from within them.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Dasein is not a fixed essence but a being that understands itself through projected possibilities. (此在不是固定本质，而是通过被筹划的可能性理解自身的存在者。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Projection (投射/筹划; de: Entwurf)** differs from **Plan (计划; de: Plan)**. A plan is a deliberate project; projection is the deeper existential opening of possibilities. (计划是有意识的项目；筹划则是更深层的生存可能性开启。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** projection prepares existentialism’s emphasis on possibility and choice, but Heidegger keeps projection tied to thrownness and finitude. (筹划为存在主义对可能性和选择的强调做准备，但海德格尔始终把筹划同被抛性和有限性相连。)  
  
### 12. Fallenness: The Problem of Everyday Absorption  
  
`Fallenness (沉沦; de: Verfallen)`  
**Definition:** Dasein’s tendency to be absorbed in everydayness, public interpretation, distraction, and the anonymous “they.” (此在沉浸于日常性、公共解释、分散状态和匿名“常人”中的倾向。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains why Dasein usually does not own its existence explicitly. (它解释为什么此在通常并不明确地把自身生存承担为自身的。)  
**Why needed:** everyday life supplies meanings and roles, but can also cover over Dasein’s ownmost possibilities. (日常生活提供意义与角色，但也可能遮蔽此在最本己的可能性。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing conformity, distraction, publicness, average understanding, or loss of existential ownership. (当分析从众、分散、公共性、平均理解或生存承担的丧失时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Fallenness does not mean moral sin. It names Dasein’s everyday absorption in the world of tasks, talk, routines, and social expectations. One lives as “one” lives. One says what “one” says. One values what “one” values.  
  
This is not simply negative. Everydayness is necessary. But it can hide the singularity of existence, especially death, responsibility, and authentic possibility.  
  
**Typical sentence:** In fallenness, Dasein understands itself through public meanings that it has not made its own. (在沉沦中，此在通过尚未被自身承担的公共意义来理解自身。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Fallenness (沉沦; de: Verfallen)** differs from **Sin (罪; la: peccatum)**. Fallenness is an existential structure of everyday absorption, not primarily a theological fault. (沉沦不同于罪；它是日常沉浸的生存结构，而不首先是神学罪责。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** fallenness anticipates later critiques of mass society, conformity, ideology, and normalized subjectivity, though Heidegger frames it existentially rather than sociologically. (沉沦预示后来对大众社会、从众、意识形态和规范化主体性的批判，尽管海德格尔以存在论而非社会学方式来表述。)  
  
### 13. The They: The Problem of Anonymous Publicness  
  
`The They (常人/人们; de: das Man)`  
**Definition:** the anonymous public way of being in which Dasein lives according to what “one” does, says, thinks, and expects. (此在按照“人们”所做、所说、所想和所期待的方式生活的匿名公共存在方式。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains how everyday norms govern Dasein without appearing as explicit commands. (它解释日常规范如何在不显现为明确命令的情况下支配此在。)  
**Why needed:** Dasein is socially immersed before it is individually self-possessed. (此在先是沉浸于社会之中，然后才可能个体地承担自身。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing public opinion, conformity, anonymity, average understanding, or normalized possibilities. (当分析公共意见、从众、匿名性、平均理解或被规范化的可能性时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
**Das Man** is not a specific group of people. It is the anonymous normativity of everyday life. It says: this is what one does; this is what one thinks; this is how one speaks; this is what matters.  
  
The They relieves Dasein of the burden of choosing itself. But it also disperses responsibility.  
  
**Typical sentence:** The They governs by making public norms appear as what “one” simply does. (常人通过使公共规范表现为“人们”只是这样做的东西而进行支配。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **The They (常人; de: das Man)** differs from **Other People (他人; de: andere Menschen)**. The They is not a set of individuals, but anonymous publicness. (常人不同于他人；它不是一组个体，而是匿名公共性。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** this concept can be read alongside later analyses of ideology, normalization, discourse, and social conformity, but its primary function is existential: it shows how Dasein loses itself in average public intelligibility. (这一概念可以同后来的意识形态、规范化、话语和社会从众分析并读，但其主要功能是存在论的：它显示此在如何在平均公共可理解性中失去自身。)  
  
### 14. Authenticity and Inauthenticity: The Problem of Owning Existence  
  
`Authenticity (本真性; de: Eigentlichkeit)`  
**Definition:** Dasein’s mode of existing in which it owns its finite possibilities rather than merely drifting in public interpretation. (此在承担自身有限可能性，而非只是漂浮于公共解释中的存在方式。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains how Dasein can retrieve itself from absorption in the They. (它解释此在如何能够从对常人的沉浸中取回自身。)  
**Why needed:** if Dasein’s being is its own issue, it can either own or evade that issue. (如果此在的存在对其自身成问题，它就可以承担或逃避这一问题。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing existential ownership, finitude, responsibility, resoluteness, or self-retrieval. (当分析生存承担、有限性、责任、决断或自我取回时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
`Inauthenticity (非本真性; de: Uneigentlichkeit)`  
**Definition:** Dasein’s mode of existing in which it lives through public meanings and avoids owning its ownmost possibilities. (此在通过公共意义生活并逃避承担其最本己可能性的存在方式。)  
**Problem solved:** it names the default everyday mode in which Dasein is dispersed into the They. (它命名此在分散于常人之中的默认日常存在方式。)  
**Why needed:** Dasein is usually absorbed in everyday publicness rather than explicitly owning its existence. (此在通常沉浸于日常公共性，而不是明确承担自身存在。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing evasion, conformity, average existence, or unowned possibility. (当分析逃避、从众、平均存在或未被承担的可能性时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Authenticity does not mean moral purity, individualistic self-expression, or being “unique.” It means owning one’s existence as finite possibility. Inauthenticity is not simple badness. It is the everyday tendency to live through inherited interpretations without taking them over as one’s own.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Authenticity is not escape from the world, but the owned inhabiting of one’s finite being-in-the-world. (本真性不是逃离世界，而是对自身有限在世存在的承担性居住。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Authenticity (本真性; de: Eigentlichkeit)** differs from **Originality (原创性; en: originality)**. Authenticity is existential ownership; originality is novelty or uniqueness. (本真性是生存承担；原创性则是新颖性或独特性。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** authenticity becomes central for existentialism, but Heidegger’s version is not primarily a theory of personal lifestyle. It is a formal existential structure of owning finite possibility. (本真性成为存在主义的核心，但海德格尔的版本并不首先是个人生活风格理论，而是承担有限可能性的形式生存结构。)  
  
### 15. Anxiety: The Problem of World-Disclosure through Uncanniness  
  
`Anxiety (焦虑; de: Angst)`  
**Definition:** a fundamental mood in which the ordinary significance of beings withdraws and Dasein is disclosed to itself as finite possibility. (一种基本情绪，其中存在者的日常意义退隐，此在作为有限可能性被开显给自身。)  
**Problem solved:** it reveals Dasein beyond everyday absorption in particular concerns. (它在日常具体操劳之外揭示此在自身。)  
**Why needed:** ordinary fear is directed at a determinate object; anxiety discloses the nothing of worldly significance and Dasein’s own being. (普通恐惧指向确定对象；焦虑则开显世界意义的无以及此在自身存在。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing existential disclosure, uncanniness, finitude, or the collapse of everyday meaning. (当分析生存开显、无家可归感、有限性或日常意义崩塌时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Anxiety is not mere psychological nervousness. It is an ontological mood. In anxiety, things do not simply become frightening. Rather, the familiar world loses its grip. What collapses is not one object, but the taken-for-granted meaningfulness of the whole.  
  
This reveals Dasein’s uncanniness: Dasein is not finally at home in the everyday world of the They.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Anxiety discloses not a threatening object, but the uncanniness of Dasein’s being-in-the-world. (焦虑开显的不是一个威胁性对象，而是此在在世存在的无家可归感。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Fear (恐惧; de: Furcht)** has a determinate object; **Anxiety (焦虑; de: Angst)** discloses the world as such and Dasein’s finite possibility. (恐惧有确定对象；焦虑开显世界本身以及此在的有限可能性。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** anxiety becomes a central existential category for later existentialism, especially in Kierkegaard, Heidegger, Sartre, and existential psychology. (焦虑成为后来存在主义的核心范畴，尤其见于克尔凯郭尔、海德格尔、萨特和存在主义心理学。)  
  
### 16. Being-toward-Death: The Problem of Ownmost Possibility  
  
`Being-toward-Death (向死而在; de: Sein-zum-Tode)`  
**Definition:** Dasein’s relation to death as its ownmost, non-relational, certain, and indefinite possibility. (此在同死亡的关系；死亡是其最本己的、不可替代的、确定而不确定何时到来的可能性。)  
**Problem solved:** it discloses Dasein’s finitude and individualizes it out of absorption in the They. (它开显此在的有限性，并使其从对常人的沉浸中个体化出来。)  
**Why needed:** Dasein can evade itself unless it confronts the possibility that cannot be outstripped or delegated. (如果不面对那种不可超越也不可委托的可能性，此在就可能逃避自身。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing mortality, finitude, authenticity, individuation, or existential urgency. (当分析死亡性、有限性、本真性、个体化或生存紧迫性时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Death is not treated here as a biological event at the end of life. It is an existential possibility that structures Dasein’s life now. Dasein is finite because its possibilities are bounded by the possibility of no-longer-being-able-to-be.  
  
This does not mean morbid obsession. It means that authentic existence requires owning finitude rather than hiding it under public clichés about death.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Being-toward-death individualizes Dasein by confronting it with the possibility that no one can take over for it. (向死而在通过使此在面对无人能代替它承担的可能性而使其个体化。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Demise (死亡事件; de: Ableben)** is biological ending; **Being-toward-Death (向死而在; de: Sein-zum-Tode)** is the existential relation to mortality. (死亡事件是生物学终结；向死而在是同死亡性的生存关系。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** Heidegger transforms death from an event in time into a structure of temporality and authenticity. Existentialism will inherit this transformation. (海德格尔把死亡从时间中的事件转化为时间性与本真性的结构。存在主义会继承这一转变。)  
  
### 17. Resoluteness: The Problem of Existential Decision  
  
`Resoluteness (决断性; de: Entschlossenheit)`  
**Definition:** Dasein’s authentic openness to its own finite possibilities in the face of thrownness, guilt, and death. (此在面对被抛性、负疚和死亡而向自身有限可能性本真开放的状态。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains how Dasein can own its existence without escaping finitude. (它解释此在如何能够承担自身存在而不逃避有限性。)  
**Why needed:** authenticity requires more than insight; it requires taking over one’s thrown possibilities. (本真性需要的不只是洞见，还需要接过自身被抛的可能性。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing decision, ownership, responsibility, finitude, or authentic action. (当分析决断、承担、责任、有限性或本真行动时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Resoluteness is not arbitrary decisionism. It is not choosing anything intensely. It means being open to the situation as one’s own and acting from owned finitude.  
  
It is tied to **Call of Conscience (良知的呼唤; de: Ruf des Gewissens)**. Conscience calls Dasein back from the They, not by giving moral rules, but by disclosing Dasein’s ownmost possibility and guilt.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Resoluteness is the taking-over of thrown possibility in the light of finitude. (决断性是在有限性之光中接过被抛可能性。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Choice (选择; de: Wahl)** can name selecting among options; **Resoluteness (决断性; de: Entschlossenheit)** names existential openness to one’s own finite possibility. (选择可以指在选项之间挑选；决断性则命名对此在自身有限可能性的生存开放。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** resoluteness influences existentialist accounts of decision and authenticity, though later thinkers often criticize its political ambiguity. (决断性影响存在主义对决断与本真性的说明，尽管后来的思想家常批评其政治暧昧性。)  
  
### 18. Temporality: The Problem of the Meaning of Dasein’s Being  
  
`Temporality (时间性; de: Zeitlichkeit)`  
**Definition:** the ecstatic structure of Dasein’s existence as thrown from the past, projecting toward the future, and involved in the present. (此在作为从过去被抛、朝向未来筹划并牵连于现在的绽出性存在结构。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains the unity of thrownness, projection, fallenness, care, and being-toward-death. (它解释被抛性、筹划、沉沦、操心和向死而在的统一。)  
**Why needed:** Dasein is not a thing located in time; its being is temporal. (此在不是位于时间中的东西；它的存在本身是时间性的。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing Dasein as future-oriented, historically thrown, and presently involved. (当分析此在作为面向未来、历史性地被抛并牵连于当下的存在时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Heidegger’s temporality is not clock time. It is not a sequence of now-points. It is ecstatic: Dasein stands out into future, past, and present. Dasein projects possibilities, has been thrown, and is absorbed in present dealings.  
  
This is why time is the horizon for understanding Being. Dasein understands Being through its temporal structure.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Dasein does not merely exist in time; Dasein exists temporally. (此在不只是存在于时间中；此在以时间性的方式存在。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Ordinary Time (通常时间; de: gewöhnliche Zeit)** is counted and measured; **Temporality (时间性; de: Zeitlichkeit)** is the existential structure through which Dasein exists. (通常时间被计数和度量；时间性是此在借以存在的生存结构。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** Heidegger radicalizes phenomenological lived time by making temporality the meaning of Dasein’s being and the horizon of the question of Being. (海德格尔激进化现象学的被生活时间，把时间性作为此在存在的意义以及存在问题的地平线。)  
  
### 19. Historicity: The Problem of Inherited Possibility  
  
`Historicity (历史性; de: Geschichtlichkeit)`  
**Definition:** Dasein’s existence as shaped by inherited possibilities, tradition, repetition, and finite projection. (此在作为由继承的可能性、传统、重复和有限筹划所塑造的存在。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains history as existential inheritance rather than mere chronology. (它把历史解释为生存性的继承，而不只是年代顺序。)  
**Why needed:** Dasein is thrown into a past that it can either repeat, evade, or transform. (此在被抛入一个过去，它可以重复、逃避或转化这个过去。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing tradition, inheritance, repetition, destiny, or historically situated existence. (当分析传统、继承、重复、命运或历史处境化生存时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Historicity means that Dasein’s possibilities are never invented from nothing. They are inherited from language, tradition, community, and history. Authenticity does not mean rejecting all inheritance. It means taking up inherited possibilities in a transformed way.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Historicity means that Dasein projects itself from possibilities it has inherited. (历史性意味着此在从其所继承的可能性中筹划自身。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **History (历史; de: Geschichte)** can mean events and development; **Historicity (历史性; de: Geschichtlichkeit)** names Dasein’s existential structure of being historically thrown. (历史可以指事件与发展；历史性命名此在作为历史性被抛者的生存结构。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** Heidegger’s historicity prepares hermeneutics and later theories of situated understanding. It also differs from Marxian historical materialism, because it treats history existentially rather than primarily through production relations. (海德格尔的历史性为解释学和后来的处境化理解理论做准备。它也不同于马克思的历史唯物主义，因为它以生存论而非主要以生产关系来处理历史。)  
  
### 20. Truth as Unconcealment: The Problem of Disclosure  
  
`Truth as Unconcealment (真理作为去蔽; el: ἀλήθεια; de: Unverborgenheit/Wahrheit)`  
**Definition:** truth understood as the disclosure or unconcealment of beings rather than merely correctness of propositions. (把真理理解为存在者的开显或去蔽，而不只是命题正确性。)  
**Problem solved:** it reopens the Greek sense of truth against the later dominance of truth as correspondence. (它反对后来真理符合论的支配，重新打开希腊意义上的真理。)  
**Why needed:** propositions can be correct only if beings are already disclosed in some way. (只有当存在者已经以某种方式被开显时，命题才可能正确。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing the prior disclosedness that makes assertion, judgment, and correctness possible. (当分析使断言、判断和正确性成为可能的先行开显性时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Heidegger does not simply reject propositional truth. He asks what makes it possible. A statement can correspond to a thing only if the thing is already disclosed as something about which one can make statements. Truth as correctness is derivative from truth as unconcealment.  
  
This returns to **Aletheia (真理/去蔽; el: ἀλήθεια)**. Truth is an event of showing, but every showing also involves concealment. Beings appear from within a clearing, not in total transparency.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Propositional truth presupposes a more originary disclosure of beings. (命题真理预设一种更原初的存在者开显。)
