**Conceptual contrast:** **Correctness (正确性; de: Richtigkeit)** concerns the agreement of statement and thing; **Unconcealment (去蔽; de: Unverborgenheit)** concerns the prior disclosure in which things can show themselves. (正确性关涉陈述与事物的一致；去蔽关涉事物得以显现的先行开显。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** Heidegger reactivates Greek **Aletheia** against Latin **Veritas (真理; la: veritas)** as correctness. Later Derrida will question whether any disclosure can escape trace, absence, and différance. (海德格尔以希腊的 Aletheia 对抗作为正确性的拉丁 Veritas。后来德里达会质疑任何开显是否能够逃离痕迹、缺席与延异。)  
  
### 21. Disclosure and Clearing: The Problem of the Open  
  
`Disclosure (开显; de: Erschlossenheit)`  
**Definition:** the openedness through which Dasein, world, and beings become intelligible. (此在、世界与存在者借以成为可理解者的开启状态。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains how beings can show up as meaningful before explicit judgment. (它解释存在者如何能在明确判断之前作为有意义者显现。)  
**Why needed:** intelligibility presupposes an open field in which beings can matter. (可理解性预设一个存在者能够有意义的开放场域。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing world-openness, meaningfulness, understanding, mood, or truth as unconcealment. (当分析世界开放性、意义性、理解、情绪或真理作为去蔽时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
`Clearing (林中空地/澄明; de: Lichtung)`  
**Definition:** the open region in which beings can appear and withdraw. (存在者能够显现并退隐的开放区域。)  
**Problem solved:** it gives a non-subjectivist account of the openness required for appearance. (它为显现所需的开放性提供一种非主体主义说明。)  
**Why needed:** appearance requires an open space of intelligibility, not merely a perceiving subject. (显现需要一个可理解性的开放空间，而不只是一个知觉主体。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing the open field in which beings are disclosed. (当分析存在者在其中被开显的开放场域时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
The clearing is one of Heidegger’s major metaphors, but it is not ornamental. A forest clearing allows things to appear in light, but also preserves shadow and concealment. Heidegger uses it to think the open as prior to subject-object relations.  
  
**Typical sentence:** The clearing is not created by a subject; it is the openness in which subject and object can first appear. (澄明并非由主体创造；它是主体与客体首先得以显现的开放性。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Lighting (照明; de: Beleuchtung)** suggests making visible by light; **Clearing (澄明; de: Lichtung)** names the open region in which visibility and concealment are possible. (照明暗示通过光使之可见；澄明命名可见与遮蔽得以可能的开放区域。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** the clearing shifts phenomenology away from consciousness toward a more originary openness of Being. (澄明把现象学从意识转向更原初的存在开放性。)  
  
### 22. Ereignis: The Problem of Appropriation  
  
`Ereignis (本有/成己事件; de: Ereignis)`  
**Definition:** the event of appropriation in which Being and human being belong together in a historical opening. (存在与人之存在在历史性开放中彼此归属的本有事件。)  
**Problem solved:** it moves beyond the framework of subject, object, and even early fundamental ontology toward the event of disclosure itself. (它超出主体、客体甚至早期基础存在论的框架，转向开显事件本身。)  
**Why needed:** later Heidegger seeks to think Being not as a static ground but as a historical giving or event. (后期海德格尔试图把存在思为历史性的给予或事件，而非静态根据。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing later Heidegger’s account of the historical event in which Being and human openness belong together. (当分析后期海德格尔关于存在与人的开放性彼此归属的历史性事件时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
**Ereignis** is difficult because it resists ordinary translation. It can suggest event, appropriation, enowning, or coming-into-one’s-own. Heidegger uses it to think the belonging-together of Being and the human being who is open to Being.  
  
The point is not that humans create Being. Nor is Being simply an object given to humans. Ereignis names a mutual appropriation: the human being is needed as the clearing for Being, and human existence is appropriated into the history of Being.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Ereignis names the event in which Being and the human openness to Being come into their belonging-together. (Ereignis 命名存在与人对存在的开放性进入彼此归属的事件。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Event (事件; de: Ereignis)** here is not merely an occurrence in time; it is the historical happening of disclosure and belonging. (这里的事件不是时间中的单纯发生，而是开显与归属的历史性发生。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** Ereignis marks Heidegger’s movement from the existential analytic of Dasein toward the history of Being. (Ereignis 标志海德格尔从此在的生存论分析转向存在历史。)  
  
### 23. Gestell: The Problem of Technological Enframing  
  
`Gestell (集置/框架化; de: Gestell/Ge-stell)`  
**Definition:** the technological mode of revealing in which beings appear as standing-reserve for ordering, use, calculation, and control. (一种技术性的揭示方式，其中存在者作为可订置、可使用、可计算和可控制的持存物显现。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains modern technology not merely as tools, but as a way in which Being is disclosed. (它把现代技术解释为一种存在被开显的方式，而不只是工具集合。)  
**Why needed:** technology changes not only what humans do, but how beings appear. (技术改变的不只是人类做什么，也改变存在者如何显现。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing technological rationality, calculability, resource-thinking, optimization, or the reduction of beings to availability. (当分析技术理性、可计算性、资源化思维、优化或存在者被化约为可用性时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
**Gestell** is one of Heidegger’s most important later terms. It does not mean a machine or device. It names the revealing structure of modern technology. Under Gestell, a river appears as hydroelectric resource, land as mineral reserve, humans as labor force or data, and time as productivity.  
  
This is why Heidegger’s critique of technology is ontological, not nostalgic. The danger is not that machines exist. The danger is that only one mode of revealing dominates: everything appears as standing-reserve.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Gestell is the technological revealing in which beings appear primarily as resources to be ordered and optimized. (集置是一种技术性揭示，在其中存在者主要作为可订置和可优化的资源显现。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Tool (工具; de: Werkzeug)** is an individual instrument; **Gestell (集置; de: Gestell)** is a historical mode of revealing. (工具是个别器具；集置是历史性的揭示方式。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** Gestell transforms critique of technology from social or moral complaint into an analysis of how modernity discloses Being. It also anticipates later critiques of instrumental reason, biopolitics, datafication, and platform control. (集置把技术批判从社会或道德抱怨转化为对现代性如何开显存在的分析。它也预示后来的工具理性、生命政治、数据化和平台控制批判。)  
  
### 24. The History of Being: The Problem of Metaphysical Epochs  
  
`History of Being (存在历史; de: Seinsgeschichte)`  
**Definition:** the historical sequence of ways in which Being is disclosed and forgotten in Western metaphysics. (存在在西方形而上学中被开显并被遗忘的历史性序列。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains metaphysics not as a series of opinions, but as epochs of disclosure. (它把形而上学解释为开显的诸时代，而不只是观点序列。)  
**Why needed:** Heidegger wants to show that different periods understand Being through different dominant determinations. (海德格尔试图显示，不同时代通过不同的主导规定来理解存在。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing how Greek, Latin, modern, technological, or nihilistic epochs disclose beings differently. (当分析希腊、拉丁、现代、技术或虚无主义时代如何以不同方式开显存在者时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
For Heidegger, Western metaphysics is not merely wrong. It is a destiny of disclosure and forgetting. Being is successively interpreted as presence, substance, actuality, objectivity, will, value, and standing-reserve. Each epoch reveals beings, but also conceals Being.  
  
This gives Heidegger’s work a genealogical dimension, though it differs from Nietzsche and Foucault. It is not primarily a genealogy of power, but a history of ontological disclosure.  
  
**Typical sentence:** The history of Being traces the changing ways in which beings are disclosed and Being is forgotten. (存在历史追踪存在者被开显以及存在被遗忘的不同方式。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Intellectual History (思想史; de: Ideengeschichte)** studies changing doctrines; **History of Being (存在历史; de: Seinsgeschichte)** studies epochs of disclosure. (思想史研究教义变化；存在历史研究开显时代。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** Heidegger turns genealogy toward ontology. Instead of asking only who produced a value or discourse, he asks how an epoch lets beings appear at all. (海德格尔把谱系学方向转向存在论。他不只追问谁生产了价值或话语，而是追问一个时代如何让存在者得以显现。)  
  
### 25. The Tool-Map of Heidegger  
  
Use Heideggerian vocabulary diagnostically. The core question is usually not “What is this object?” but “How is Being disclosed here?”  
  
**If the text asks who can ask the question of Being**, look for **Dasein (此在; de: Dasein)** and **Fundamental Ontology (基础存在论; de: Fundamentalontologie)**.  
(如果文本追问谁能够提出存在问题，应寻找此在与基础存在论问题。)  
  
**If the text distinguishes entities from their Being**, look for **Being (存在; de: Sein)**, **Beings (存在者; de: Seiendes)**, and **Ontological Difference (存在论差异; de: ontologische Differenz)**.  
(如果文本区分存在者与其存在，应寻找存在、存在者和存在论差异问题。)  
  
**If the text rejects the inner subject/outer object model**, look for **Being-in-the-world (在世存在; de: In-der-Welt-sein)** and **World (世界; de: Welt)**.  
(如果文本拒绝内部主体/外部对象模型，应寻找在世存在与世界问题。)  
  
**If the text analyzes tools, use, and practice**, look for **Ready-to-Hand (上手状态; de: Zuhandenheit)**, **Present-at-Hand (现成在手状态; de: Vorhandenheit)**, and **Equipment (器具; de: Zeug)**.  
(如果文本分析工具、使用和实践，应寻找上手状态、现成在手状态与器具问题。)  
  
**If the text analyzes Dasein’s existential structure**, look for **Care (操心; de: Sorge)**, **Thrownness (被抛性; de: Geworfenheit)**, **Projection (筹划; de: Entwurf)**, and **Fallenness (沉沦; de: Verfallen)**.  
(如果文本分析此在的生存结构，应寻找操心、被抛性、筹划和沉沦问题。)  
  
**If the text analyzes everyday conformity**, look for **The They (常人; de: das Man)**, **Everydayness (日常性; de: Alltäglichkeit)**, and **Inauthenticity (非本真性; de: Uneigentlichkeit)**.  
(如果文本分析日常从众，应寻找常人、日常性与非本真性问题。)  
  
**If the text analyzes finitude and self-ownership**, look for **Anxiety (焦虑; de: Angst)**, **Being-toward-Death (向死而在; de: Sein-zum-Tode)**, **Authenticity (本真性; de: Eigentlichkeit)**, and **Resoluteness (决断性; de: Entschlossenheit)**.  
(如果文本分析有限性和自我承担，应寻找焦虑、向死而在、本真性与决断性问题。)  
  
**If the text asks how truth is more than correctness**, look for **Unconcealment (去蔽; el: ἀλήθεια; de: Unverborgenheit)**, **Disclosure (开显; de: Erschlossenheit)**, and **Clearing (澄明; de: Lichtung)**.  
(如果文本追问真理如何不只是正确性，应寻找去蔽、开显与澄明问题。)  
  
**If the text concerns later Heidegger**, look for **Ereignis (本有/成己事件; de: Ereignis)**, **Gestell (集置; de: Gestell)**, and **History of Being (存在历史; de: Seinsgeschichte)**.  
(如果文本涉及后期海德格尔，应寻找 Ereignis、集置和存在历史问题。)  
  
### 26. The Genealogical Point of Part 8  
  
Heidegger transforms phenomenology into an inquiry into Being. Husserl asks how objects are given to consciousness. Heidegger asks how beings are disclosed in a world and how the meaning of Being has been forgotten in metaphysics. His language is not merely difficult style; it is a tool for breaking inherited grammar. Ordinary words such as **world**, **truth**, **care**, **being**, and **time** become technical because the ordinary metaphysical use of language already hides the problem.  
  
The guiding thesis is:  
  
**Heideggerian language turns philosophy from the analysis of objects to the disclosure of Being: to understand a thing is to ask how it shows up within a world, for Dasein, under a historical opening of Being.**  
(海德格尔式语言把哲学从对象分析转向存在开显：理解一个事物，就是追问它如何在一个世界中、对作为此在的存在者、在存在的历史性开放下显现。)  
  
This grammar changes everything that follows. Existentialism inherits Dasein’s finitude, possibility, anxiety, and authenticity, but often translates them into freedom and choice. Hermeneutics inherits world, historicity, and understanding. Derrida inherits Heidegger’s destruction of metaphysics but questions whether Being can be retrieved without trace and différance. Foucault differs sharply from Heidegger, but both treat modernity as a historical formation that determines what can appear and count as truth. **Genealogy (谱系学; de: Genealogie; fr: généalogie)** traces the contingent historical formation of ideas, and **Power/Knowledge (权力/知识; fr: savoir-pouvoir; en: power/knowledge)** names the inseparability of power relations and knowledge production; Heidegger’s parallel contribution is to ask how historical epochs disclose Being itself.  
  
The Heideggerian question remains one of the strongest tools for philosophical reading:  
  
**What mode of Being is silently presupposed when this text speaks of objects, subjects, truth, technology, or world?**  
(当这个文本谈论对象、主体、真理、技术或世界时，它默默预设了什么存在方式？)  
  
## Part 9. Existentialism: Freedom, Project, Bad Faith  
  
This chapter explains existentialist language as a practical grammar of finite freedom. Heidegger had analyzed **Dasein (此在; de: Dasein)** through being-in-the-world, thrownness, projection, anxiety, authenticity, and being-toward-death. Existentialism inherits this terrain but shifts the center of pressure. The decisive question becomes: **if human existence is not secured by a fixed essence, divine order, rational system, or natural telos, how must one live, choose, and take responsibility?** (如果人的存在不再由固定本质、神圣秩序、理性体系或自然目的保证，那么人必须如何生活、选择并承担责任？)  
  
The central vocabulary is **Existence**, **Essence**, **Existence precedes essence**, **Freedom**, **Choice**, **Responsibility**, **Project**, **Situation**, **Facticity**, **Transcendence**, **Bad Faith**, **Nothingness**, **Anguish**, **The Other**, **The Look**, **Absurd**, **Revolt**, and **Ambiguity**. **Existence precedes essence (存在先于本质; fr: l’existence précède l’essence)** names Sartre’s reversal of the traditional priority of essence, and **Mauvaise foi (自欺; fr: mauvaise foi)** names self-deception about one’s freedom.  
  
The operational function of this chapter is exact: use existentialist vocabulary when the problem is **not what human nature is**, but **how a finite being without fixed essence lives its freedom under conditions it did not choose**. (当问题不是“人的本性是什么”，而是“一个没有固定本质的有限存在者如何在并非由自己选择的条件下活出自由”时，应使用存在主义词汇。)  
  
### 1. The Problem-Situation: From Being to Existence  
  
Existentialism emerges after several major collapses. Classical metaphysics had treated human beings through **Essence (本质; la: essentia)**, **Soul (灵魂; el: ψυχή; la: anima)**, **Nature (自然; el: φύσις; la: natura)**, or **Reason (理性; la: ratio; de: Vernunft)**. Christian metaphysics had situated human life within creation, sin, grace, and providence. German Idealism had interpreted freedom within spirit, history, and rational reconciliation. Nietzsche had announced the crisis of inherited values through **Death of God (上帝之死; de: Tod Gottes)** and **Nihilism (虚无主义; de: Nihilismus)**.  
  
Existentialism asks what remains after these guarantees weaken.  
  
The central question is:  
  
**How can a human being exist without a predetermined essence and yet still be responsible for becoming someone?**  
(人如何能够在没有预定本质的情况下存在，却仍然对成为某种人负责？)  
  
This question changes philosophical grammar. A human being is not first a thing with a fixed definition. A human being is a task, a project, a risk, a freedom, and a responsibility. Existence is not merely a fact. It is a burden of self-formation.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Existentialism treats the human being not as a fixed nature, but as a finite project that must become itself through choices. (存在主义不把人视为固定本性，而是把人视为一种必须通过选择成为自身的有限筹划。)  
  
### 2. Existence: The Problem of Being as Lived Task  
  
`Existence (存在/实存; la: existentia; fr: existence; de: Existenz)`  
**Definition:** the concrete, lived, finite way in which a human being is there and must become itself. (人具体地、被生活地、有限地在那里并必须成为自身的方式。)  
**Problem solved:** it shifts attention from abstract essence to lived self-making. (它把注意力从抽象本质转向被生活的自我形成。)  
**Why needed:** human life cannot be fully understood as the instantiation of a pre-given definition. (人的生活不能被充分理解为预先给定定义的实例化。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing human life as concrete, finite, chosen, situated, and unfinished. (当分析人的生活作为具体的、有限的、被选择的、处境化的和未完成的存在时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Existence is not merely “being there” in the thin sense that a stone exists. Existentialist existence names the way a human being has to live its being. A stone is what it is. A tool has a function given within a practice. But a human being must take a stand on what it is to be.  
  
This is why existentialist language is practical before it is theoretical. To exist is not only to be describable. It is to be implicated in one’s own becoming.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Existence names the fact that the human being is not simply given, but must live itself as a task. (存在命名这样一个事实：人并不是简单被给予的东西，而是必须把自身作为任务来生活。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Existence (存在/实存; fr: existence)** differs from **Mere Presence (单纯在场; de: Vorhandenheit)**. Mere presence means being there as an object; existence means living one’s being as possibility and responsibility. (单纯在场意味着作为对象在那里；实存意味着把自身存在作为可能性和责任来生活。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** existence moves from a metaphysical predicate to a lived problem. Latin metaphysics had distinguished essence and existence; existentialism turns that distinction into a drama of freedom. (存在从形而上学谓词变成被生活的问题。拉丁形而上学区分本质与存在；存在主义把这一区分转化为自由的戏剧。)  
  
### 3. Essence: The Problem of Fixed Definition  
  
`Essence (本质; la: essentia; fr: essence; de: Wesen)`  
**Definition:** what a thing is, or the defining structure that makes it the kind of thing it is. (某物是什么，或使其成为该类事物的规定性结构。)  
**Problem solved:** in classical metaphysics, essence explains identity, function, and definition. (在古典形而上学中，本质解释同一性、功能与定义。)  
**Why needed:** without essence, many objects cannot be classified or defined. (如果没有本质，许多对象就无法被分类或定义。)  
**How to use:** in existentialism, use it critically when analyzing attempts to define human beings in advance. (在存在主义中，当分析预先定义人的尝试时，应批判性地使用这一概念。)  
  
Existentialism does not deny that essences can apply to artifacts or biological classifications. A knife may have a function before it is made. A triangle may be defined by its structure. But existentialism contests the idea that human beings have a ready-made essence that determines what they must be.  
  
The danger of essence is that it can become an excuse. “That is just what I am.” “That is my role.” “That is human nature.” “That is what society made me.” These claims may contain facts, but existentialism asks whether they are being used to evade freedom.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Essence becomes oppressive when it is used to treat human freedom as already defined. (当本质被用来把人的自由视为已经被定义之物时，本质就变得压迫性。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Essence (本质; fr: essence)** gives definition; **Existence (存在/实存; fr: existence)** names the unfinished act of becoming. (本质给出定义；存在/实存命名未完成的生成活动。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** the older metaphysical priority of essence becomes the target of existential reversal. The question is no longer “what is the human essence?” but “how does a human being become what it is without hiding behind essence?” (古老的本质优先性成为存在主义反转的靶子。问题不再是“人的本质是什么？”，而是“人在不躲藏于本质背后的情况下如何成为其所是者？”)  
  
### 4. Existence Precedes Essence: The Problem of Radical Reversal  
  
`Existence Precedes Essence (存在先于本质; fr: l’existence précède l’essence)`  
**Definition:** the thesis that human beings first exist and only later define themselves through action, choice, and project. (人首先存在，然后才通过行动、选择和筹划定义自身的命题。)  
**Problem solved:** it reverses the traditional view that human nature or essence determines human life in advance. (它反转了人的本性或本质预先规定人生的传统观点。)  
**Why needed:** if there is no pre-given human essence, responsibility cannot be transferred to nature, God, society, or destiny. (如果没有预先给定的人类本质，责任就不能被转移给自然、上帝、社会或命运。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing human self-definition, responsibility, anti-essentialism, or the refusal of fixed human nature. (当分析人的自我定义、责任、反本质主义或对固定人性的拒绝时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
This is Sartre’s most famous formula, but it should not be treated as a slogan only. It is a weapon against excuses. If existence precedes essence, then the human being cannot say: “my nature made me this.” One may have a body, a history, a class, a gendered situation, a family, a language, and constraints. But none of these fully cancels the burden of taking a position.  
  
This does not mean that one can become anything whatsoever. Existentialism is not fantasy voluntarism. It means that meaning is not settled in advance. One must respond to one’s situation.  
  
**Typical sentence:** If existence precedes essence, then a human being is not defined before acting, but becomes defined through acting. (如果存在先于本质，那么人在行动之前并未被定义，而是通过行动成为被定义者。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Essentialism (本质主义; fr: essentialisme)** treats identity as fixed by nature or definition; **Existentialism (存在主义; fr: existentialisme)** treats human identity as a project under conditions. (本质主义把身份视为由自然或定义固定；存在主义把人的身份视为条件之下的筹划。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** the essence/existence distinction moves from scholastic metaphysics into modern ethical and political critique. It becomes a tool against determinism, role-fixation, and naturalized identity. (本质/存在区分从经院形而上学转入现代伦理与政治批判，成为反对决定论、角色固定和身份自然化的工具。)  
  
### 5. Freedom: The Problem of Unavoidable Choice  
  
`Freedom (自由; fr: liberté; de: Freiheit)`  
**Definition:** the condition in which a human being must choose itself through its acts, even under constraints. (人在约束之下仍必须通过自身行动选择自身的状态。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains responsibility without relying on a fixed essence or external moral script. (它在不依赖固定本质或外部道德剧本的情况下解释责任。)  
**Why needed:** if human beings are not predefined, they must take up their existence through choice. (如果人不是预先被定义的，人就必须通过选择接过自身存在。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing decision, responsibility, self-definition, evasion, or the burden of possibility. (当分析决断、责任、自我定义、逃避或可能性的负担时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Existentialist freedom is not primarily political liberty, though it has political consequences. It is ontological and practical. A human being cannot avoid taking a stance. Even refusal, passivity, obedience, and silence can function as choices.  
  
This makes freedom burdensome. It is not merely the pleasant ability to do what one wants. It is the fact that one is answerable for what one makes of what has been made of one.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Freedom is not the absence of conditions; it is the responsibility of taking up one’s conditions in a project. (自由不是没有条件，而是在一个筹划中接过自身条件的责任。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Freedom (自由; fr: liberté)** differs from **License (任意; la: licentia)**. License means doing whatever one happens to desire; existential freedom means being responsible for the meaning of one’s acts. (任意意味着做碰巧想做的事；存在主义自由意味着对自身行动的意义负责。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** freedom moves from Kantian autonomy as rational self-legislation to existential self-making under contingency. (自由从康德式作为理性自我立法的自主性，转向偶然性条件下的生存自我形成。)  
  
### 6. Choice: The Problem of Self-Definition through Action  
  
`Choice (选择; fr: choix; de: Wahl)`  
**Definition:** the act through which a human being commits itself to a possibility and thereby gives itself a determinate shape. (人借以把自身投入一种可能性并由此赋予自身确定形态的活动。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains how an undefined existence becomes a concrete life. (它解释未被定义的存在如何成为具体人生。)  
**Why needed:** without choice, freedom remains abstract and unrealized. (如果没有选择，自由就保持抽象且未现实化。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing action as self-forming commitment rather than merely preference selection. (当把行动分析为形成自我的承诺，而不只是偏好选择时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Existentialist choice is deeper than selecting between options. It is self-committing. To choose is to disclose what one takes to matter. A choice gives shape not only to a future but also to the chooser.  
  
This is why existentialism treats even ordinary decisions seriously. A life is not built only from dramatic heroic choices. It is formed through repeated patterns of commitment, evasion, compromise, courage, and refusal.  
  
**Typical sentence:** In choosing an act, one also chooses a way of being. (在选择一个行动时，人也选择一种存在方式。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Preference (偏好; fr: préférence)** expresses what one likes; **Choice (选择; fr: choix)** commits one to a possibility and its meaning. (偏好表达喜欢什么；选择则把人投入一种可能性及其意义。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** choice becomes the existential form of **Projection (筹划; de: Entwurf)**. Heidegger analyzes projection structurally; existentialism turns it into the concrete drama of decision. (选择成为筹划的存在主义形式。海德格尔结构性地分析筹划；存在主义把它转化为决断的具体戏剧。)  
  
### 7. Responsibility: The Problem of Owning One’s Freedom  
  
`Responsibility (责任; fr: responsabilité; de: Verantwortung)`  
**Definition:** answerability for what one makes of oneself and one’s situation through action. (人通过行动把自身和自身处境变成什么的可回应性。)  
**Problem solved:** it prevents freedom from becoming mere spontaneity or excuse-making. (它防止自由变成单纯自发性或制造借口。)  
**Why needed:** if one chooses, one must answer for the meaning and consequences of one’s choices. (如果人进行选择，就必须对选择的意义和后果负责。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing moral burden, answerability, complicity, evasion, or collective implication. (当分析道德负担、可回应性、共谋、逃避或集体牵连时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Responsibility is the other side of freedom. Existentialism refuses the comfort of saying: “I had no choice.” Sometimes constraints are severe; sometimes choices are tragic; sometimes every available option is compromised. But existentialism insists that one still takes a stance.  
  
This does not mean blaming victims for oppression. It means that existence always involves a relation to what happens. One can submit, resist, reinterpret, flee, deny, endure, or act with others. Responsibility names this unavoidable relation to one’s situated freedom.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Responsibility means that one cannot separate oneself from the meaning one gives to one’s acts. (责任意味着人不能把自身同其赋予自身行动的意义分离开。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Causation (因果性; la: causalitas)** explains why something happened; **Responsibility (责任; fr: responsabilité)** asks how an agent is answerable for acting within conditions. (因果性解释某事为何发生；责任追问行动者如何在条件中对行动负责。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** responsibility becomes post-metaphysical. It is not grounded in a fixed cosmic order, but in the structure of freedom itself. (责任成为后形而上学的。它不再奠基于固定宇宙秩序，而是奠基于自由结构本身。)  
  
### 8. Project: The Problem of Life as Direction  
  
`Project (筹划/项目; fr: projet; de: Entwurf)`  
**Definition:** the organizing orientation through which a human being gives shape to its life by pursuing possibilities. (人通过追求可能性而赋予自身生活形态的组织性取向。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains the unity of a life without appealing to fixed essence. (它在不诉诸固定本质的情况下解释人生的统一性。)  
**Why needed:** if the self has no ready-made essence, its unity must be produced through projects. (如果自我没有现成的本质，其统一性就必须通过筹划来生产。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing life-orientation, self-definition, future-directedness, vocation, or existential commitment. (当分析生活取向、自我定义、未来指向、使命或生存承诺时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
A project is not merely a practical plan. It is an existential orientation. One’s project may be to become a writer, to avoid risk, to dominate others, to be loved, to obey, to appear innocent, to serve truth, to survive, or to refuse humiliation. Often the project is not fully explicit.  
  
Existential analysis asks what project unifies scattered acts. The question is not only “what did this person do?” but “what way of being is disclosed by these acts?”  
  
**Typical sentence:** A project gives a life its direction by organizing possibilities into a way of being. (筹划通过把可能性组织成一种存在方式而赋予生活方向。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Project (筹划; fr: projet)** differs from **Goal (目标; fr: but)**. A goal can be achieved and finished; a project organizes the meaning of a life over time. (目标可以被达成并结束；筹划则在时间中组织人生意义。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** project translates Heidegger’s existential projection into Sartrean self-definition. It also becomes useful for analyzing vocation, identity, political commitment, and self-narration. (筹划把海德格尔的生存投射转化为萨特式自我定义，也适用于分析使命、身份、政治承诺和自我叙事。)  
  
### 9. Situation: The Problem of Freedom under Conditions  
  
`Situation (处境; fr: situation; de: Situation)`  
**Definition:** the concrete field of facts, constraints, relations, histories, and possibilities within which freedom acts. (自由在其中行动的由事实、约束、关系、历史和可能性构成的具体场域。)  
**Problem solved:** it prevents existential freedom from becoming abstract or disembodied. (它防止存在主义自由变成抽象的或脱离身体的自由。)  
**Why needed:** freedom is always exercised somewhere, by someone, with a body, history, language, class, gender, and world. (自由总是在某处、由某人、带着身体、历史、语言、阶级、性别和世界被行使。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing how freedom is constrained, enabled, shaped, or burdened by concrete conditions. (当分析自由如何被具体条件限制、开启、塑造或加重负担时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Situation is essential because existentialism is often misunderstood as unlimited self-creation. A situation is the field within which freedom must act. It includes one’s body, birth, past, social position, political conditions, others, material constraints, and historical moment.  
  
Freedom does not cancel situation. It takes a position within it.  
  
**Typical sentence:** A situation limits freedom, but it also gives freedom the concrete field in which it can act. (处境限制自由，但也为自由提供能够行动的具体场域。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Situation (处境; fr: situation)** differs from **Determinism (决定论; fr: déterminisme)**. Situation conditions freedom; determinism denies freedom by making action fully caused. (处境规定自由的条件；决定论则通过使行动完全由原因决定来否认自由。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** situation links existentialism with social and political critique. Beauvoir, Fanon, and later feminist and postcolonial thought will use situated freedom to criticize abstract universal accounts of the subject. (处境把存在主义同社会和政治批判连接起来。波伏娃、法农以及后来的女性主义和后殖民思想会用处境化自由批判抽象普遍主体理论。)  
  
### 10. Facticity and Transcendence: The Problem of Being Both Given and Beyond  
  
`Facticity (事实性; fr: facticité; de: Faktizität)`  
**Definition:** the given facts of one’s existence, including body, past, social position, death, and historical condition. (自身存在的被给予事实，包括身体、过去、社会位置、死亡和历史条件。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains the non-chosen side of existence. (它解释存在中非选择的一面。)  
**Why needed:** freedom does not begin from nothing; it begins from facts already there. (自由不是从虚无开始，而是从已经在那里的事实开始。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing what constrains or conditions human freedom. (当分析限制或规定人类自由条件的东西时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
`Transcendence (超越; fr: transcendance; de: Transzendenz)`  
**Definition:** the movement by which human existence goes beyond given facts toward possibilities. (人的存在超出被给予事实而朝向可能性的运动。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains why human beings are not reducible to what they already are. (它解释为什么人不能被化约为其已经如此的状态。)  
**Why needed:** without transcendence, facticity becomes determinism. (如果没有超越，事实性就会变成决定论。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing possibility, self-projection, future-directed action, or refusal to be reduced to facts. (当分析可能性、自我筹划、面向未来的行动或拒绝被化约为事实时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
The pair **facticity/transcendence** is one of the most useful existentialist tools. Human beings are facts and more than facts. One has a body, a past, a place, a language, and constraints. But one also takes a stance toward these facts.  
  
Bad faith often consists in collapsing this tension. One may pretend to be only facticity: “I am nothing but my role, my past, my nature.” Or one may pretend to be pure transcendence: “My situation does not matter; I am completely free.” Both evasions distort existence.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Human existence is the unstable unity of facticity and transcendence. (人的存在是事实性与超越之间不稳定的统一。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Facticity (事实性; fr: facticité)** is what is given; **Transcendence (超越; fr: transcendance)** is the movement beyond the given toward possibility. (事实性是被给予者；超越是超出被给予者而朝向可能性的运动。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** this pair reworks Heidegger’s **Thrownness (被抛性; de: Geworfenheit)** and **Projection (筹划; de: Entwurf)** into a Sartrean structure of freedom and constraint. (这一对概念把海德格尔的被抛性与筹划改写成萨特式自由与约束结构。)  
  
### 11. Bad Faith: The Problem of Self-Deception about Freedom  
  
`Bad Faith (自欺; fr: mauvaise foi)`  
**Definition:** self-deception in which a person denies either freedom or facticity in order to evade responsibility. (一种自我欺骗：人否认自由或事实性，以逃避责任。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains how a free being can hide its own freedom from itself. (它解释一个自由存在者如何能够向自身隐藏自身自由。)  
**Why needed:** existentialism needs a concept for evasion that is neither simple ignorance nor deliberate lying. (存在主义需要一个概念来解释既非简单无知也非蓄意撒谎的逃避。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing role-identification, excuse-making, self-objectification, denial of responsibility, or false innocence. (当分析角色认同、找借口、自我对象化、否认责任或虚假无辜时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Bad faith is subtle because the deceiver and deceived are the same person. A person both knows and does not know their freedom. They hide from what they are doing by identifying too fully with a role, a fact, a social mask, or an abstract freedom.  
  
Classic forms of bad faith include:  
  
“I am only my job.” (我只是我的工作。)  
“I had no choice.” (我别无选择。)  
“My feelings made me do it.” (我的感受让我这么做。)  
“My situation does not affect me at all.” (我的处境完全不影响我。)  
  
Each statement may contain partial truth. Bad faith begins when partial truth is used to evade the full structure of existence.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Bad faith is the attempt to become either a thing without freedom or a freedom without facts. (自欺就是试图变成没有自由的物，或没有事实性的自由。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Lying (说谎; fr: mensonge)** deceives another person; **Bad Faith (自欺; fr: mauvaise foi)** is self-deception about one’s own freedom and situation. (说谎欺骗他人；自欺则是在自身自由与处境问题上的自我欺骗。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** bad faith transforms Heidegger’s inauthenticity into a more explicit theory of self-deception, role-performance, and responsibility. (自欺把海德格尔的非本真性转化为更明确的自我欺骗、角色表演和责任理论。)  
  
### 12. Nothingness: The Problem of Negation within Existence  
  
`Nothingness (虚无; fr: néant; de: Nichts)`  
**Definition:** the negativity through which consciousness separates itself from what is and opens possibility. (意识借以同既有之物分离并开启可能性的否定性。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains how freedom can negate facts, distance itself from being, and imagine alternatives. (它解释自由如何能够否定事实、同存在保持距离并想象替代可能。)  
**Why needed:** if human beings were fully identical with what they are, choice and transformation would be impossible. (如果人完全等同于其所是，选择与转化就不可能。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing negation, absence, possibility, freedom, or the gap between consciousness and being. (当分析否定、缺席、可能性、自由或意识与存在之间的裂缝时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
For Sartre, consciousness is not a solid thing. It is a lack, distance, or nothingness within being. It can say no. It can imagine what is not. It can take distance from what exists. This negativity makes freedom possible.  
  
Nothingness is therefore not merely emptiness. It is the structure of separation that allows consciousness not to be identical with its facts.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Nothingness is the gap through which consciousness is not simply identical with what it is. (虚无是意识不简单等同于其所是的裂缝。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Being-in-itself (自在存在; fr: être-en-soi)** is full, inert, and identical with itself; **Being-for-itself (自为存在; fr: être-pour-soi)** is consciousness as lack, negation, and self-transcendence. (自在存在是充实的、惰性的、同自身同一的；自为存在则是作为缺乏、否定和自我超越的意识。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** nothingness radicalizes Hegelian negation and Heideggerian anxiety. It becomes the ontological structure of freedom. (虚无激进化黑格尔式否定与海德格尔式焦虑，成为自由的存在论结构。)  
  
### 13. Anguish: The Problem of Experiencing Freedom  
  
`Anguish (焦虑/苦恼; fr: angoisse; de: Angst)`  
**Definition:** the affective experience of recognizing that one is free and responsible without ultimate external guarantee. (意识到自身在没有最终外部保证的情况下是自由且负责时的情感经验。)  
**Problem solved:** it shows that freedom is not merely empowering but also disturbing. (它显示自由不只是赋权性的，也是令人不安的。)  
**Why needed:** if nothing fully determines one’s choice, then one must bear the weight of choosing. (如果没有东西完全决定人的选择，人就必须承受选择的重量。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing the burden, vertigo, or unease of freedom. (当分析自由的负担、眩晕或不安时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Existential anguish differs from ordinary fear. Fear has an object: a dog, a threat, a loss. Anguish concerns freedom itself. One experiences that no rule, role, or essence can choose in one’s place.  
  
This is why anguish is not merely negative. It can disclose freedom. It shows that one is not simply carried by the world.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Anguish is the feeling of being unable to escape responsibility for one’s freedom. (焦虑/苦恼是无法逃避自身自由责任的感受。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Fear (恐惧; fr: peur)** concerns a determinate threat; **Anguish (焦虑/苦恼; fr: angoisse)** concerns the burden of freedom itself. (恐惧关涉确定威胁；焦虑/苦恼关涉自由本身的负担。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** anguish translates Heideggerian **Anxiety (焦虑; de: Angst)** into a more explicitly ethical and existential experience of responsibility. (焦虑/苦恼把海德格尔式焦虑转化为更明确的伦理性和生存性责任经验。)  
  
### 14. The Other: The Problem of Being Exposed  
  
`The Other (他者; fr: autrui; de: der Andere)`  
**Definition:** another consciousness before whom one appears and by whom one can be judged, recognized, objectified, or threatened. (另一个意识；人在其面前显现，并可能被其判断、承认、对象化或威胁。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains why selfhood is not private self-possession but exposure to others. (它解释为什么自我性不是私人自我占有，而是暴露于他者。)  
**Why needed:** one’s identity is shaped not only by choice but also by how one appears to others. (人的身份不仅由选择塑造，也由其如何向他者显现而塑造。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing shame, recognition, conflict, objectification, desire, or social identity. (当分析羞耻、承认、冲突、对象化、欲望或社会身份时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Existentialism does not treat the self as isolated. Other people are not just external objects. They reveal a dimension of selfhood that one cannot control: one is visible, interpreted, judged, and possibly objectified.  
  
This produces conflict. The other can recognize one’s freedom, but can also freeze one into an object, role, stereotype, or identity.  
  
**Typical sentence:** The other reveals that I am not only a freedom for myself, but also an object in another’s world. (他者揭示：我不只是对自身而言的自由，也是在他者世界中的对象。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Intersubjectivity (主体间性; de: Intersubjektivität)** emphasizes shared world and mutual relation; **The Other (他者; fr: autrui)** in Sartrean analysis often emphasizes exposure, conflict, and objectification. (主体间性强调共享世界与相互关系；萨特式他者分析常强调暴露、冲突和对象化。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** the problem of the other links existentialism to recognition theory, psychoanalysis, feminism, postcolonial thought, and social ontology. (他者问题把存在主义同承认理论、精神分析、女性主义、后殖民思想和社会本体论连接起来。)  
  
### 15. The Look: The Problem of Objectification  
  
`The Look/Gaze (凝视; fr: regard)`  
**Definition:** the experience of being seen by another and thereby becoming an object for another consciousness. (被另一个意识看见并由此成为另一个意识之对象的经验。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains shame, objectification, exposure, and the instability of selfhood. (它解释羞耻、对象化、暴露和自我性的不稳定。)  
**Why needed:** selfhood is not fully controlled from within because one also exists for others. (自我性并不完全由内部控制，因为人也为他者而存在。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing shame, social visibility, gendered objectification, racialization, surveillance, or interpersonal conflict. (当分析羞耻、社会可见性、性别化对象化、种族化、监视或人际冲突时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
The Look is not just physical seeing. It is the structure of being made an object in another’s field of meaning. A person caught peeping through a keyhole suddenly experiences themselves as seen. Shame reveals that one has become an object for another.  
  
This concept is powerful because it links ontology, affect, and social power. To be seen is not always neutral. The look can classify, judge, sexualize, racialize, discipline, or humiliate.  
  
**Typical sentence:** The Look reveals my being-for-others by making me experience myself as an object in another’s world. (凝视通过使我把自身经验为他者世界中的对象而揭示我的为他存在。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Seeing (看见; fr: voir)** is a perceptual act; **The Look (凝视; fr: regard)** is the existential structure of being exposed to another’s objectifying consciousness. (看见是知觉活动；凝视则是暴露于他者对象化意识中的生存结构。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** the Look becomes crucial for later theories of gender, race, surveillance, coloniality, media, and visual power. (凝视成为后来性别、种族、监视、殖民性、媒体和视觉权力理论的重要概念。)  
  
### 16. Ambiguity: The Problem of Being Both Subject and Object  
  
`Ambiguity (暧昧性/两义性; fr: ambiguïté)`  
**Definition:** the condition of human existence as both free and situated, subject and object, facticity and transcendence. (人的存在同时是自由的和处境化的、主体和客体、事实性和超越的状态。)  
**Problem solved:** it prevents existentialism from simplifying human life into pure freedom or pure determination. (它防止存在主义把人类生活简化为纯自由或纯决定。)  
**Why needed:** human beings are neither things nor gods; they are finite freedoms in a shared world. (人既不是物，也不是神；人是共享世界中的有限自由。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing ethical conflict, oppression, gender, embodiment, dependence, or situated freedom. (当分析伦理冲突、压迫、性别、具身性、依赖或处境化自由时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Ambiguity is especially important in Simone de Beauvoir’s existential ethics. Human beings are ambiguous because they are both subjects who transcend and bodies situated among others. Denying either side produces distortion. Pure transcendence ignores oppression and embodiment. Pure facticity denies freedom.  
  
Ambiguity is therefore not a defect to eliminate. It is the structure that ethics must face.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Existential ethics begins from ambiguity: human beings are free, but only as embodied and situated beings among others. (存在主义伦理学从暧昧性出发：人是自由的，但只是作为在他者之中的具身且处境化存在者而自由。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Ambiguity (暧昧性; fr: ambiguïté)** differs from **Confusion (混乱; fr: confusion)**. Ambiguity is a structural duality of existence, not merely unclear thinking. (暧昧性不同于混乱；它是存在的结构性双重性，而不只是思维不清。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** ambiguity allows existentialism to move beyond heroic individualism toward feminist, ethical, and political analysis of situated freedom. (暧昧性使存在主义超出英雄式个人主义，转向对处境化自由的女性主义、伦理学和政治分析。)  
  
### 17. Oppression: The Problem of Freedom Denied by Situation  
  
`Oppression (压迫; fr: oppression)`  
**Definition:** a social condition in which some persons’ freedom is constrained, objectified, or denied by structures created and maintained by others. (某些人的自由被他者创造并维持的结构所限制、对象化或否认的社会状态。)  
**Problem solved:** it prevents existential freedom from ignoring social domination. (它防止存在主义自由忽视社会支配。)  
**Why needed:** if all humans are free only in situation, unjust situations can systematically deform freedom. (如果所有人都只在处境中自由，不正义处境就可能系统性地扭曲自由。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing how social structures limit the possibilities through which persons can become themselves. (当分析社会结构如何限制人得以成为自身的可能性时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Existentialism becomes politically serious when it recognizes that freedom is not evenly situated. A person oppressed by gender, race, colonial domination, class, or violence still has freedom, but that freedom operates within constrained and often hostile possibilities.  
  
This is why simplistic existentialism is inadequate. Telling someone “you are free” without analyzing oppression can become another form of bad faith. Freedom must be understood materially, socially, and historically.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Oppression does not erase freedom, but it structures the field of possibilities in which freedom must act. (压迫并不抹除自由，但它结构化自由必须在其中行动的可能性场域。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Constraint (限制; fr: contrainte)** may be any limitation; **Oppression (压迫; fr: oppression)** is a socially structured and unjust limitation of freedom. (限制可以是任何约束；压迫则是社会结构化且不正义的自由限制。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** existentialism here converges with Marxian, feminist, anticolonial, and critical theory. Freedom is no longer only individual choice; it becomes a problem of world-structure. (在这里，存在主义同马克思主义、女性主义、反殖民和批判理论汇合。自由不再只是个体选择，而成为世界结构问题。)  
  
### 18. Absurd: The Problem of Meaning without Cosmic Answer  
  
`Absurd (荒诞; fr: absurde)`  
**Definition:** the confrontation between the human demand for meaning and the world’s refusal to provide a final answer. (人对意义的需求同世界拒绝提供最终答案之间的对峙。)  
**Problem solved:** it names the condition of seeking meaning in a world without guaranteed meaning. (它命名在没有被保证意义的世界中寻求意义的状态。)  
**Why needed:** after the collapse of transcendent guarantees, meaning cannot be simply inherited. (在超越保证崩塌之后，意义不能被简单继承。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing meaning-crisis, cosmic silence, existential lucidity, or life without final justification. (当分析意义危机、宇宙沉默、生存清醒或没有最终证成的生活时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Camus gives the absurd a distinct function. The absurd is not merely that life is meaningless. It arises from a relation: humans ask for meaning, unity, and justification; the world gives no final answer. The absurd is the clash.  
  
The absurd does not automatically lead to despair. It can produce lucidity. One sees the absence of final guarantee and refuses false consolation.  
  
**Typical sentence:** The absurd is not in the human alone or the world alone, but in their confrontation. (荒诞不单独在人之中，也不单独在世界之中，而在二者的对峙中。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Nihilism (虚无主义; de: Nihilismus)** concerns the collapse of value-authority; **Absurd (荒诞; fr: absurde)** concerns the clash between human meaning-demand and world-silence. (虚无主义关涉价值权威的崩塌；荒诞关涉人的意义需求与世界沉默之间的冲突。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** absurdity translates Nietzsche’s post-metaphysical crisis into a lived confrontation with meaninglessness. (荒诞把尼采的后形而上学危机转化为同无意义的被生活的对峙。)  
  
### 19. Revolt: The Problem of Living without Final Justification  
  
`Revolt (反抗; fr: révolte)`  
**Definition:** the lucid refusal to submit to absurdity, oppression, or false consolation while continuing to act. (在清醒中拒绝屈从于荒诞、压迫或虚假安慰，同时继续行动。)  
**Problem solved:** it offers an ethical response to absurdity that is neither suicide, resignation, nor metaphysical escape. (它为荒诞提供一种伦理回应，既不是自杀、屈从，也不是形而上学逃避。)  
**Why needed:** if no final meaning is given, existence must still be lived and affirmed through action. (如果没有最终意义被给予，存在仍必须通过行动被生活和肯定。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing resistance, dignity, solidarity, refusal, or action without guarantee. (当分析抵抗、尊严、团结、拒绝或没有保证的行动时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Revolt is not mere rebellion against authority. It is a way of living the absurd without surrendering to it. One refuses both despair and false hope. This refusal can become ethical and political, especially when revolt recognizes shared vulnerability.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Revolt is the decision to act without final guarantee and without false consolation. (反抗是在没有最终保证且没有虚假安慰的情况下行动的决断。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Revolution (革命; fr: révolution)** seeks structural overthrow; **Revolt (反抗; fr: révolte)** names a stance of refusal that may be existential, ethical, or political. (革命寻求结构性推翻；反抗命名一种拒绝姿态，它可以是生存的、伦理的或政治的。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** revolt converts absurdity into ethical energy. It links existentialism with resistance literature, anticolonial struggle, and political ethics. (反抗把荒诞转化为伦理能量，并把存在主义同抵抗文学、反殖民斗争和政治伦理连接起来。)  
  
### 20. Commitment: The Problem of Acting without Foundations  
  
`Commitment (介入/承诺; fr: engagement)`  
**Definition:** the act of taking responsibility for a position, cause, work, or relation within history. (在历史中对一种立场、事业、作品或关系承担责任的行动。)  
**Problem solved:** it prevents freedom from remaining abstract, aesthetic, or purely inward. (它防止自由停留为抽象的、审美化的或纯内在的自由。)  
**Why needed:** existence becomes concrete through commitments that bind a person to others and to the world. (存在通过把人与他者和世界连接起来的承诺而变得具体。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing political responsibility, artistic practice, ethical action, public speech, or historical agency. (当分析政治责任、艺术实践、伦理行动、公共言说或历史行动者性时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Commitment is a key bridge between existentialism and politics. If human beings are free, they cannot remain neutral spectators. Even noncommitment may function as commitment to the status quo.  
  
For Sartre, writing, politics, love, and action are not merely private expressions. They are ways of taking responsibility in a shared historical world.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Commitment is freedom made concrete in a historical situation. (介入/承诺是自由在历史处境中的具体化。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Neutrality (中立; fr: neutralité)** claims non-involvement; **Commitment (介入; fr: engagement)** recognizes that existence is already implicated. (中立声称不介入；介入则承认存在总是已经被牵连。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** commitment turns existentialism toward public responsibility, literature, politics, and collective struggle. (介入把存在主义转向公共责任、文学、政治和集体斗争。)  
  
### 21. The Tool-Map of Existentialism  
  
Use existentialist vocabulary diagnostically. The core question is usually not “What is human nature?” but “How is this person, group, or text negotiating freedom under conditions?”  
  
**If the text rejects fixed human nature**, look for **Existence (存在/实存; fr: existence)**, **Essence (本质; fr: essence)**, and **Existence Precedes Essence (存在先于本质; fr: l’existence précède l’essence)**.  
(如果文本拒绝固定人性，应寻找存在、本质和存在先于本质问题。)  
  
**If the text analyzes self-formation through action**, look for **Freedom (自由; fr: liberté)**, **Choice (选择; fr: choix)**, **Responsibility (责任; fr: responsabilité)**, and **Project (筹划; fr: projet)**.  
(如果文本分析通过行动进行自我形成，应寻找自由、选择、责任和筹划问题。)  
  
**If the text analyzes freedom under constraints**, look for **Situation (处境; fr: situation)**, **Facticity (事实性; fr: facticité)**, and **Transcendence (超越; fr: transcendance)**.  
(如果文本分析约束条件下的自由，应寻找处境、事实性和超越问题。)  
  
**If the text analyzes evasion of freedom**, look for **Bad Faith (自欺; fr: mauvaise foi)** and **Role-Identification (角色认同; en: role-identification)**.  
(如果文本分析对自由的逃避，应寻找自欺与角色认同问题。)  
  
**If the text analyzes negativity and possibility**, look for **Nothingness (虚无; fr: néant)**, **Being-in-itself (自在存在; fr: être-en-soi)**, and **Being-for-itself (自为存在; fr: être-pour-soi)**.  
(如果文本分析否定性与可能性，应寻找虚无、自在存在和自为存在问题。)  
  
**If the text analyzes affective disclosure of freedom**, look for **Anguish (焦虑/苦恼; fr: angoisse)** and **Anxiety (焦虑; de: Angst)**.  
(如果文本分析自由的情感性开显，应寻找焦虑/苦恼问题。)  
  
**If the text analyzes social exposure and objectification**, look for **The Other (他者; fr: autrui)** and **The Look (凝视; fr: regard)**.  
(如果文本分析社会暴露与对象化，应寻找他者与凝视问题。)  
  
**If the text analyzes situated freedom politically**, look for **Ambiguity (暧昧性; fr: ambiguïté)**, **Oppression (压迫; fr: oppression)**, and **Commitment (介入; fr: engagement)**.  
(如果文本以政治方式分析处境化自由，应寻找暧昧性、压迫和介入问题。)  
  
**If the text analyzes meaning after metaphysical collapse**, look for **Absurd (荒诞; fr: absurde)**, **Revolt (反抗; fr: révolte)**, and **Nihilism (虚无主义; de: Nihilismus)**.  
(如果文本分析形而上学崩塌之后的意义问题，应寻找荒诞、反抗和虚无主义问题。)  
  
### 22. The Genealogical Point of Part 9  
  
Existentialism transforms ontology into a grammar of lived responsibility. Heidegger had shown that Dasein is finite, thrown, projected, and being-toward-death. Sartre, Beauvoir, Camus, and other existentialist thinkers translate this terrain into the language of freedom, choice, responsibility, bad faith, ambiguity, absurdity, revolt, and commitment.  
  
The guiding thesis is:  
  
**Existentialist language turns human existence into a problem of situated freedom: to understand a person is not to identify a fixed essence, but to analyze how that person takes up facts, possibilities, others, and history through choices and evasions.**  
(存在主义语言把人的存在转化为处境化自由的问题：理解一个人，不是识别固定本质，而是分析此人如何通过选择与逃避接过事实、可能性、他者和历史。)  
  
This grammar becomes crucial for later philosophy. Feminist existentialism uses situation and ambiguity to criticize abstract accounts of freedom. Anticolonial thought uses the look, objectification, and oppression to analyze racialized existence. Psychoanalysis and structuralism challenge existentialism’s account of consciousness and freedom. Foucault will later ask how subjects are historically produced through practices and discourses, complicating existential self-making. Derrida will destabilize any final self-presence of the subject. Yet existentialism leaves a durable question that later critique cannot easily escape:  
  
**Even if the subject is historically produced, how does it live, choose, resist, or evade within that production?**  
(即使主体是历史地被生产出来的，它仍如何在这种生产中生活、选择、抵抗或逃避？)  
  
## Part 10. Analytic Philosophy: Argument, Logic, Reference  
  
This chapter explains analytic philosophy as a language of argumentative control. Earlier chapters moved through Being, essence, subjectivity, critique, phenomenology, existential freedom, and genealogy. Analytic philosophy changes the toolset. Its primary question is not first **how Being is disclosed**, **how consciousness intends**, or **how values are historically produced**. Its core question is: **what exactly is being claimed, what follows from it, and under what conditions would it be true or false?** (核心问题是：究竟提出了什么主张？什么从中推出？在什么条件下它为真或为假？)  
  
The central vocabulary is **Argument**, **Premise**, **Conclusion**, **Inference**, **Validity**, **Soundness**, **Entailment**, **Necessary Condition**, **Sufficient Condition**, **Definition**, **Counterexample**, **Thought Experiment**, **Conceptual Analysis**, **Use/Mention**, **Sense**, **Reference**, **Proposition**, **Truth-Value**, **Possible World**, **Necessity**, **Possibility**, and **Supervenience**. Analytic philosophy emphasizes clarity, economy, explicit argumentative structure, and terms such as **argument**, **premise**, **conclusion**, **validity**, **soundness**, **necessary/sufficient condition**, and **counterexample**.  
  
The operational function of this chapter is precise: use analytic vocabulary when the problem is **not primarily historical depth or existential disclosure**, but **logical structure, conceptual precision, argument evaluation, truth-conditions, and inferential control**. (当问题不主要是历史深度或生存开显，而是逻辑结构、概念精确性、论证评估、真值条件和推论控制时，应使用分析哲学词汇。)  
  
### 1. The Problem-Situation: From Philosophical Depth to Philosophical Control  
  
Analytic philosophy arises from dissatisfaction with obscurity, speculative excess, psychologism, metaphysical inflation, and uncontrolled abstraction. It does not deny that philosophy can address deep problems. It asks that depth be made answerable to clarity.  
  
The central question becomes:  
  
**Can this philosophical problem be clarified by analyzing the language, logic, conditions, or inferential structure of the claims involved?**  
(这个哲学问题能否通过分析相关主张的语言、逻辑、条件或推论结构而被澄清？)  
  
This question changes philosophical style. A philosophical text becomes less a grand historical movement and more a controlled sequence of claims. The reader asks:  
  
What is the thesis?  
(论题是什么？)  
  
What premises support it?  
(哪些前提支持它？)  
  
Does the conclusion follow?  
(结论是否推出？)  
  
Are the key terms defined?  
(核心术语是否已被定义？)  
  
Is there a counterexample?  
(是否存在反例？)  
  
Are necessary and sufficient conditions confused?  
(是否混淆了必要条件与充分条件？)  
  
What exactly would make this sentence true?  
(究竟什么会使这个句子为真？)  
  
Analytic language is therefore not shallow. It is disciplinary. It forces philosophical claims to become inspectable.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Analytic philosophy turns philosophical depth into claims that can be defined, tested, formalized, objected to, and revised. (分析哲学把哲学深度转化为可以被定义、检验、形式化、反驳和修订的主张。)  
  
### 2. Argument: The Problem of Giving Reasons  
  
`Argument (论证; la: argumentum; en: argument)`  
**Definition:** a structured set of claims in which some claims are offered as reasons for another claim. (一组结构化主张，其中某些主张被作为另一个主张的理由提出。)  
**Problem solved:** it distinguishes philosophical reasoning from assertion, rhetoric, association, or impression. (它把哲学推理同断言、修辞、联想或印象区分开来。)  
**Why needed:** philosophy requires not only claims, but reasons that can be examined. (哲学不仅需要主张，还需要可被检验的理由。)  
**How to use:** use it when identifying the structure by which a thesis is supported. (当识别一个论题如何被支持的结构时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
An argument is not a quarrel. It is a reason-giving structure. In analytic reading, the first task is often to reconstruct the argument, even if the text does not state it formally.  
  
A basic argument has:  
  
**Premises (前提; la: praemissae; en: premises)**  
**Conclusion (结论; la: conclusio; en: conclusion)**  
**Inference (推论; la: inferentia; en: inference)**  
  
For example:  
  
If all knowledge requires justification, and perception can provide justification, then perception can contribute to knowledge. (如果一切知识都需要证成，而知觉能够提供证成，那么知觉能够参与知识形成。)  
  
This is not yet enough. The analytic question is whether the premises are true and whether the conclusion follows.  
  
**Typical sentence:** An argument is not evaluated by whether it sounds profound, but by whether its conclusion is supported by its premises. (一个论证的评估不取决于它听起来是否深刻，而取决于其结论是否由前提支持。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Assertion (断言; la: assertio)** states that something is the case; **Argument (论证; en: argument)** gives reasons for why it is the case. (断言说明某事为真；论证给出为什么它为真的理由。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** analytic philosophy transforms philosophy from a discourse of insight into a practice of accountable reasons. (分析哲学把哲学从洞见话语转化为可问责理由的实践。)  
  
### 3. Premise and Conclusion: The Problem of Argument Structure  
  
`Premise (前提; la: praemissa; en: premise)`  
**Definition:** a claim offered as support for another claim. (作为支持另一主张而提出的主张。)  
**Problem solved:** it identifies what an argument depends on. (它识别论证依赖什么。)  
**Why needed:** without identifying premises, one cannot know where to test an argument. (如果不识别前提，就无法知道应在哪里检验论证。)  
**How to use:** use it when reconstructing the reasons on which a conclusion rests. (当重构结论所依赖的理由时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
`Conclusion (结论; la: conclusio; en: conclusion)`  
**Definition:** the claim that an argument aims to establish. (论证试图确立的主张。)  
**Problem solved:** it identifies what the argument is trying to prove. (它识别论证试图证明什么。)  
**Why needed:** without identifying the conclusion, a reader may confuse background, illustration, objection, and thesis. (如果不识别结论，读者可能混淆背景、例子、反驳和论题。)  
**How to use:** use it when locating the central claim supported by the argument. (当定位由论证支持的中心主张时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Analytic reading often begins by marking premise indicators and conclusion indicators.  
  
Premise indicators include: **because**, **since**, **given that**, **for**, **assuming that**. (前提标记包括 because、since、given that、for、assuming that。)  
  
Conclusion indicators include: **therefore**, **thus**, **hence**, **so**, **it follows that**. (结论标记包括 therefore、thus、hence、so、it follows that。)  
  
Analytic style also depends on explicit discourse markers such as **therefore**, **however**, **suppose**, and **hence** for tracking philosophical argument.  
  
**Typical sentence:** To understand an analytic text, first separate what is being argued for from what is being used to argue for it. (理解分析哲学文本时，首先要区分被论证的东西与用来论证它的东西。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Premise (前提; en: premise)** is a supporting claim; **Conclusion (结论; en: conclusion)** is the supported claim. (前提是支持性主张；结论是被支持的主张。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** the premise/conclusion distinction makes philosophical reading more surgical. It replaces broad thematic appreciation with structural reconstruction. (前提/结论区分使哲学阅读更具解剖性，用结构重构取代宽泛主题欣赏。)  
  
### 4. Inference: The Problem of Moving from Claims to Claims  
  
`Inference (推论; la: inferentia; en: inference)`  
**Definition:** the movement from one or more claims to another claim. (从一个或多个主张走向另一个主张的过程。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains how conclusions are drawn from premises. (它解释结论如何从前提中得出。)  
**Why needed:** an argument is not just a list of claims; it depends on relations of support. (论证不只是主张列表；它依赖支持关系。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing whether a conclusion really follows from what has been stated. (当分析结论是否真正从已陈述内容推出时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Inference is the hinge between premises and conclusion. Two arguments may use the same words but differ in inferential structure. This is why analytic philosophy often reconstructs arguments into numbered form.  
  
For example:  
  
1. If mental states are identical with brain states, then two beings with identical brain states have identical mental states.  
2. It is possible for two beings to have identical brain states but different conscious experiences.  
3. Therefore, mental states are not identical with brain states.  
   (1. 如果心理状态等同于脑状态，那么两个具有相同脑状态的存在者具有相同心理状态。2. 两个存在者可能具有相同脑状态却有不同意识经验。3. 因此，心理状态不等同于脑状态。)  
  
One may reject premise 2, or dispute the modal claim, or challenge the inference. The structure makes disagreement precise.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Inference is the path by which an argument moves from what is granted to what is claimed. (推论是论证从被承认之物走向被主张之物的路径。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Inference (推论; en: inference)** differs from **Association (联想; en: association)**. Association connects ideas psychologically; inference connects claims rationally. (联想在心理上连接观念；推论在理性上连接主张。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** inference gives analytic philosophy its procedural character. The question becomes not only what a thinker says, but what the thinker is licensed to infer. (推论赋予分析哲学以程序性。问题不仅是思想家说了什么，还包括思想家被允许推出什么。)  
  
### 5. Validity: The Problem of Formal Consequence  
  
`Validity (有效性; la: validitas; en: validity)`  
**Definition:** a property of an argument such that if the premises are true, the conclusion must be true. (一种论证性质：如果前提为真，则结论必然为真。)  
**Problem solved:** it separates the structure of an argument from the actual truth of its premises. (它把论证结构同前提的实际真假区分开来。)  
**Why needed:** an argument can have correct form even if its premises are false. (即使前提为假，一个论证也可能具有正确形式。)  
**How to use:** use it when testing whether the conclusion follows from the premises. (当检验结论是否从前提推出时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Validity is one of the core analytic tools. It does not mean that the conclusion is true. It means that the conclusion follows if the premises are true.  
  
For example:  
  
All cats are reptiles.  
All reptiles are philosophers.  
Therefore, all cats are philosophers.  
(所有猫都是爬行动物。所有爬行动物都是哲学家。因此，所有猫都是哲学家。)  
  
This argument is valid in form, but its premises are false. Validity concerns form, not factual correctness.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Validity asks whether the conclusion must follow, not whether the premises are actually true. (有效性追问结论是否必然推出，而不是前提是否实际为真。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Validity (有效性; en: validity)** differs from **Truth (真; en: truth)**. Truth applies to propositions; validity applies to arguments. (真适用于命题；有效性适用于论证。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** validity formalizes a central philosophical demand: reasoning must be accountable not only in content, but in structure. (有效性把哲学的一个核心要求形式化：推理不仅在内容上要可问责，在结构上也要可问责。)  
  
### 6. Soundness: The Problem of Validity plus Truth  
  
`Soundness (可靠性/健全性; en: soundness)`  
**Definition:** a property of an argument that is valid and has all true premises. (一种论证性质：该论证有效，并且所有前提为真。)  
**Problem solved:** it combines good logical form with true starting points. (它把良好逻辑形式与真实出发点结合起来。)  
**Why needed:** validity alone does not guarantee truth if the premises are false. (如果前提为假，单靠有效性并不能保证结论为真。)  
**How to use:** use it when evaluating whether an argument not only follows correctly but also begins from true claims. (当评估一个论证不仅是否正确推出，而且是否从真实主张出发时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Soundness is stronger than validity. A sound argument cannot have a false conclusion. If an argument is valid and all its premises are true, the conclusion must be true.  
  
This creates a two-step test:  
  
First, test validity: does the conclusion follow?  
(第一，检验有效性：结论是否推出？)  
  
Second, test premise truth: are the premises true?  
(第二，检验前提真性：前提是否为真？)  
  
**Typical sentence:** A sound argument is a valid argument with true premises. (可靠/健全论证是一个具有真实前提的有效论证。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Valid but Unsound (有效但不可靠; en: valid but unsound)** means the form works but at least one premise is false. (有效但不可靠意味着形式成立，但至少一个前提为假。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** soundness makes disagreement more exact. One can say: “I accept the inference but reject premise 2.” (可靠性使分歧更精确。可以说：“我接受这个推论，但拒绝第二前提。”)  
  
### 7. Deduction, Induction, and Abduction: The Problem of Types of Support  
  
`Deduction (演绎; la: deductio; en: deduction)`  
**Definition:** reasoning in which the conclusion follows necessarily from the premises if the argument is valid. (在有效论证中结论从前提必然推出的推理。)  
**Problem solved:** it provides maximal logical security. (它提供最高程度的逻辑安全性。)  
**Why needed:** some philosophical claims require necessity rather than probability. (某些哲学主张需要必然性而非概率。)  
**How to use:** use it when evaluating strict entailment. (当评估严格蕴含时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
`Induction (归纳; la: inductio; en: induction)`  
**Definition:** reasoning from observed cases to a general pattern or future expectation. (从已观察案例推向一般模式或未来预期的推理。)  
**Problem solved:** it supports empirical generalization. (它支持经验性概括。)  
**Why needed:** much knowledge depends on patterns rather than strict logical necessity. (许多知识依赖模式，而不是严格逻辑必然性。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing generalization, evidence, probability, or empirical expectation. (当分析概括、证据、概率或经验预期时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
`Abduction (溯因/最佳解释推理; en: abduction/inference to the best explanation)`  
**Definition:** reasoning to the hypothesis that best explains the available evidence. (推向最能解释现有证据之假说的推理。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains how inquiry can justify hypotheses when strict proof is unavailable. (它解释在没有严格证明时探究如何证成假说。)  
**Why needed:** science, history, law, and everyday reasoning often rely on explanatory fit. (科学、历史、法律和日常推理常依赖解释上的契合。)  
**How to use:** use it when comparing explanatory hypotheses. (当比较解释性假说时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Not all support is deductive. This matters because many bad critiques attack an inductive or abductive argument for failing to be deductively valid. That is a category mistake. Each type of inference has different standards.  
  
**Typical sentence:** A deductive argument aims at necessity, an inductive argument aims at probability, and an abductive argument aims at explanatory superiority. (演绎论证追求必然性，归纳论证追求概率，溯因论证追求解释优势。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Proof (证明; en: proof)** is stronger than **Evidence (证据; en: evidence)**. Proof may establish a conclusion decisively; evidence supports a conclusion to some degree. (证明强于证据。证明可以决定性地确立结论；证据则以某种程度支持结论。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** analytic philosophy clarifies that “reason” is not one thing. Different arguments require different standards of assessment. (分析哲学澄清“理性”并非单一之物。不同论证需要不同评估标准。)  
  
### 8. Entailment: The Problem of What Follows  
  
`Entailment (蕴含; en: entailment)`  
**Definition:** a relation in which the truth of one claim guarantees the truth of another. (一个主张为真保证另一个主张为真的关系。)  
**Problem solved:** it identifies strict consequence between propositions. (它识别命题之间的严格后承关系。)  
**Why needed:** philosophy often turns on what a thesis commits one to. (哲学常取决于一个论题使人承诺什么。)  
**How to use:** use it when asking what must be accepted if a claim is accepted. (当追问如果接受一个主张就必须接受什么时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Entailment is the logic of commitment. If a position entails a contradiction, it is in trouble. If it entails a surprising but acceptable consequence, the position becomes clearer. If it does not entail what critics say it entails, the criticism fails.  
  
For example, “All mental events are physical events” may entail that there are no non-physical mental events. But it does not automatically entail that consciousness is unreal. That further conclusion would require additional premises.  
  
**Typical sentence:** To analyze entailment is to ask what a claim commits one to, whether one notices it or not. (分析蕴含就是追问一个主张使人承诺什么，无论其是否意识到这一点。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Entailment (蕴含; en: entailment)** differs from **Association (联想; en: association)** and **Implication in ordinary speech (暗示; en: implication)**. Entailment is strict logical consequence; ordinary implication can be contextual suggestion. (蕴含不同于联想和日常语言中的暗示。蕴含是严格逻辑后承；日常暗示可能只是语境提示。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** entailment makes philosophical positions accountable for their consequences. A theory is not judged only by its intentions, but by what follows from it. (蕴含使哲学立场必须对其后果负责。理论不仅按其意图被判断，也按其推出内容被判断。)  
  
### 9. Necessary and Sufficient Conditions: The Problem of Conceptual Boundaries  
  
`Necessary Condition (必要条件; en: necessary condition)`  
**Definition:** a condition without which something cannot be the case. (没有它某事就不可能成立的条件。)  
**Problem solved:** it identifies what must be present for a concept or state to apply. (它识别一个概念或状态适用时必须存在的东西。)  
**Why needed:** many philosophical errors confuse what is required with what is enough. (许多哲学错误混淆了所必需者与足够者。)  
**How to use:** use it when asking what a concept cannot apply without. (当追问缺少什么一个概念就不能适用时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
`Sufficient Condition (充分条件; en: sufficient condition)`  
**Definition:** a condition that, if present, guarantees that something is the case. (如果它存在，就保证某事成立的条件。)  
**Problem solved:** it identifies what is enough for a concept or state to apply. (它识别什么足以使一个概念或状态适用。)  
**Why needed:** a feature may be required without being enough, or enough without being required. (某个特征可能是必需但不足够的，也可能是足够但非必需的。)  
**How to use:** use it when asking what guarantees the application of a concept. (当追问什么保证一个概念适用时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
This distinction is one of the most practical analytic tools.  
  
Example:  
  
Being unmarried is a necessary condition for being a bachelor. (未婚是成为单身汉的必要条件。)  
Being unmarried is not a sufficient condition for being a bachelor, because unmarried children and unmarried women are not bachelors under the ordinary definition. (未婚不是成为单身汉的充分条件，因为未婚儿童和未婚女性在通常定义下不是单身汉。)  
  
The full definition might say: being an unmarried adult male is sufficient for being a bachelor, under ordinary usage. (在通常用法下，未婚成年男性足以成为单身汉。)  
  
**Typical sentence:** A necessary condition is required; a sufficient condition is enough. (必要条件是所必需者；充分条件是足以成立者。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Necessary (必要; en: necessary)** does not mean **important (重要; en: important)**. A condition may be necessary in the logical sense even if it is not the most explanatorily important feature. (必要并不等于重要。一个条件可以在逻辑上必要，但并不是解释上最重要的特征。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** necessary/sufficient analysis turns definition into a testable structure. It allows philosophy to ask whether a proposed analysis is too broad, too narrow, or circular. (必要/充分分析把定义转化为可检验结构，使哲学能够追问一个分析是否过宽、过窄或循环。)  
  
### 10. Definition: The Problem of Conceptual Control  
  
`Definition (定义; el: ὁρισμός; la: definitio; en: definition)`  
**Definition:** a statement of the conditions under which a term or concept applies. (一个术语或概念适用条件的陈述。)  
**Problem solved:** it gives inquiry control over meaning and scope. (它使探究能够控制意义与适用范围。)  
**Why needed:** without definition, disagreement may be verbal rather than substantive. (如果没有定义，分歧可能只是语言性的而非实质性的。)  
**How to use:** use it when clarifying what a term includes, excludes, or requires. (当澄清一个术语包含什么、排除什么或要求什么时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Definitions are not always final. They are instruments. A definition can be proposed, tested, revised, or rejected. Analytic philosophy often treats definitions as hypotheses about conceptual use.  
  
A good definition should avoid several defects:  
  
It should not be **too broad**. (不应过宽。)  
It should not be **too narrow**. (不应过窄。)  
It should not be **circular**. (不应循环。)  
It should not smuggle in what it needs to prove. (不应偷渡它需要证明的内容。)  
  
**Typical sentence:** A definition is a tool for controlling when a concept applies and when it does not. (定义是控制一个概念何时适用、何时不适用的工具。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Definition (定义; en: definition)** differs from **Example (例子; en: example)**. An example illustrates a concept; a definition states its conditions. (例子说明概念；定义陈述其条件。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** analytic definition continues the Greek search for **Form/Essence (形式/本质; el: εἶδος; la: essentia)**, but makes it procedural: propose conditions, test cases, revise. (分析式定义延续希腊对形式/本质的追问，但使其程序化：提出条件，测试案例，修订。)  
  
### 11. Counterexample: The Problem of Testing General Claims  
  
`Counterexample (反例; en: counterexample)`  
**Definition:** a case that satisfies a proposed condition while violating the intended conclusion, or a case that shows a general claim to be false. (一个满足某拟议条件却违反预期结论的案例，或一个显示一般主张为假的案例。)  
**Problem solved:** it tests definitions, principles, and universal claims. (它检验定义、原则和全称主张。)  
**Why needed:** a single well-formed counterexample can defeat an unrestricted universal claim. (一个构造良好的反例可以击败一个无限制的全称主张。)  
**How to use:** use it when testing whether a theory covers all and only the right cases. (当检验一个理论是否覆盖所有且仅覆盖正确案例时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Counterexamples are central to analytic method. If someone says “knowledge is justified true belief,” Gettier-style cases ask whether a person can have justified true belief and still lack knowledge. If yes, the definition is insufficient.  
  
The counterexample does not merely refute. It diagnoses. It shows what the proposed definition failed to capture.  
  
**Typical sentence:** A counterexample shows where a principle’s apparent generality breaks. (反例显示一个原则表面上的普遍性在哪里断裂。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Objection (反驳/异议; en: objection)** can be broad; **Counterexample (反例; en: counterexample)** is a specific case designed to test a claim. (异议可以很宽泛；反例则是为检验一个主张而设计的具体案例。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** counterexample method makes philosophy experimental in a conceptual sense. It uses imagined or actual cases to stress-test concepts. (反例方法使哲学在概念意义上具有实验性。它使用想象或实际案例来压力测试概念。)  
  
### 12. Thought Experiment: The Problem of Testing Intuitions  
  
`Thought Experiment (思想实验; de: Gedankenexperiment; en: thought experiment)`  
**Definition:** an imagined scenario used to test concepts, principles, intuitions, or theoretical commitments. (一种用于测试概念、原则、直觉或理论承诺的想象场景。)  
**Problem solved:** it allows philosophy to isolate variables that ordinary cases mix together. (它允许哲学分离日常案例中混杂在一起的变量。)  
**Why needed:** many philosophical issues cannot be tested directly by ordinary observation alone. (许多哲学问题不能仅由普通观察直接检验。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing whether a concept still applies under unusual but structured conditions. (当分析一个概念在异常但有结构的条件下是否仍然适用时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Thought experiments are not mere stories. They are controlled conceptual devices. The point is not whether the scenario is realistic in every detail, but what it reveals about a concept.  
  
Examples include brains in vats, trolley cases, Mary the color scientist, zombies, twin earth, ship of Theseus, and veil of ignorance scenarios. Each tests a philosophical boundary: knowledge, ethics, consciousness, reference, identity, or justice.  
  
**Typical sentence:** A thought experiment is a controlled imaginary case designed to reveal what a concept commits us to. (思想实验是一种受控的想象案例，旨在揭示一个概念使我们承诺什么。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Fiction (虚构; en: fiction)** may aim at narrative effect; **Thought Experiment (思想实验; en: thought experiment)** aims at conceptual testing. (虚构可以追求叙事效果；思想实验追求概念检验。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** thought experiments continue the Socratic practice of testing definitions through cases, but sharpen it into a modern analytic tool. (思想实验延续苏格拉底通过案例测试定义的实践，但将其强化为现代分析工具。)  
  
### 13. Intuition: The Problem of Pre-Theoretical Judgment  
  
`Intuition (直觉; en: intuition)`  
**Definition:** a pre-theoretical judgment or seeming about a case, concept, or principle. (关于某个案例、概念或原则的前理论判断或似真感。)  
**Problem solved:** it gives analytic philosophy data for testing concepts when empirical measurement is not the issue. (当问题不是经验测量时，它为分析哲学提供检验概念的数据。)  
**Why needed:** conceptual analysis often begins from what competent speakers or thinkers judge about cases. (概念分析常从有能力的说话者或思考者对案例的判断出发。)  
**How to use:** use it when assessing whether a theory matches considered judgments about cases. (当评估一个理论是否符合关于案例的审慎判断时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Analytic intuitions are not mystical insights. They are judgments about cases. For example, in a Gettier case, many people have the intuition that the subject lacks knowledge despite having justified true belief. The intuition pressures the definition.  
  
But intuitions are contested. They may be culturally variable, theoretically contaminated, unstable, or unreliable. Later analytic philosophy often debates how much weight intuitions should carry.  
  
**Typical sentence:** An intuition is a pre-theoretical judgment that a case does or does not fall under a concept. (直觉是一个案例是否落入某个概念之下的前理论判断。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Intuition (直觉; en: intuition)** in analytic philosophy differs from **Intuition (直观; de: Anschauung)** in Kant. Kantian intuition is immediate givenness; analytic intuition is a judgment or seeming about a case. (分析哲学中的直觉不同于康德的直观。康德式直观是直接给予性；分析哲学中的直觉是关于案例的判断或似真感。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** intuition becomes both a tool and a problem. Analytic philosophy uses intuitions but also increasingly questions their reliability. (直觉既成为工具，也成为问题。分析哲学使用直觉，同时也越来越质疑其可靠性。)  
  
### 14. Conceptual Analysis: The Problem of What We Mean  
  
`Conceptual Analysis (概念分析; en: conceptual analysis)`  
**Definition:** the method of clarifying a concept by identifying its conditions, implications, contrasts, and applications. (通过识别概念的条件、蕴含、对照和适用范围来澄清概念的方法。)  
**Problem solved:** it turns vague philosophical questions into more precise questions about meaning and use. (它把模糊的哲学问题转化为关于意义与使用的更精确问题。)  
**Why needed:** many philosophical disputes arise from confused or unstable concepts. (许多哲学争论来自混乱或不稳定的概念。)  
**How to use:** use it when asking what it means to know, act freely, be responsible, refer, be conscious, or be identical over time. (当追问知道、自由行动、负责、指称、有意识或跨时间同一究竟意味着什么时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Conceptual analysis is not simply dictionary work. It asks how a concept functions in reasoning. What counts as knowledge? What makes an action free? What is a person? What is causation? What is justice? These questions require conditions, cases, distinctions, and counterexamples.  
  
The danger is over-idealization. A concept may not have clean necessary and sufficient conditions. Ordinary language may be open-textured. Social concepts may be contested. Later analytic philosophy often modifies classical conceptual analysis for this reason.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Conceptual analysis asks what must be true for a concept to apply correctly. (概念分析追问为了使一个概念正确适用，什么必须为真。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Conceptual Analysis (概念分析; en: conceptual analysis)** differs from **Etymology (词源学; el: ἔτυμον)**. Etymology traces word origin; conceptual analysis tests current conceptual function. (词源学追踪词源；概念分析检验当前概念功能。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** conceptual analysis differs from genealogy. Genealogy asks how a concept was historically produced; conceptual analysis asks how a concept functions in meaning, inference, and application. Both can be combined, but they answer different questions. (概念分析不同于谱系学。谱系学追问概念如何被历史生产；概念分析追问概念如何在意义、推论和适用中运作。二者可以结合，但回答不同问题。)  
  
### 15. Use and Mention: The Problem of Language-Level Confusion  
  
`Use/Mention Distinction (使用/提及区分; en: use/mention distinction)`  
**Definition:** the distinction between using a word to talk about something and mentioning the word itself. (使用一个词来谈论某物与提及该词本身之间的区分。)  
**Problem solved:** it prevents confusion between language and what language refers to. (它防止语言同语言所指之物之间发生混淆。)  
**Why needed:** many philosophical confusions arise when one slides between talking about things and talking about words. (许多哲学混乱来自在谈论事物与谈论词语之间滑动。)  
**How to use:** use it when clarifying whether a sentence concerns an object, a concept, a term, or a linguistic expression. (当澄清一个句子涉及对象、概念、术语还是语言表达时，应使用这一区分。)  
  
Example:  
  
Socrates is mortal.  
(苏格拉底是会死的。)  
  
“Socrates” has eight letters.  
(“Socrates” 有八个字母。)  
  
The first sentence uses the word to talk about the person. The second mentions the word itself.  
  
This distinction is simple but powerful. Without it, a reader may confuse claims about reality with claims about vocabulary.  
  
**Typical sentence:** To use a word is to apply it; to mention a word is to talk about the word itself. (使用一个词是应用它；提及一个词是谈论该词本身。)
