**Conceptual contrast:** **Object-Language (对象语言; en: object-language)** talks about things; **Meta-Language (元语言; en: meta-language)** talks about language. (对象语言谈论事物；元语言谈论语言。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** the use/mention distinction reflects analytic philosophy’s broader linguistic discipline: many metaphysical-looking problems may depend on shifts in language-level. (使用/提及区分体现分析哲学更广泛的语言纪律：许多看似形而上学的问题可能依赖语言层级的滑动。)  
  
### 16. Sense and Reference: The Problem of Meaning and Object  
  
`Sense (涵义; de: Sinn; en: sense)`  
**Definition:** the mode of presentation by which a referent is given in thought or language. (指称对象在思想或语言中被给予的呈现方式。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains how two expressions can refer to the same thing while differing in cognitive significance. (它解释两个表达如何能够指称同一事物，却具有不同认知意义。)  
**Why needed:** reference alone cannot explain informative identity statements. (单靠指称无法解释有信息量的同一陈述。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing meaning beyond mere object-reference. (当分析超出单纯对象指称的意义时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
`Reference (指称; de: Bedeutung; en: reference)`  
**Definition:** the object, entity, or value to which an expression refers. (一个表达所指向的对象、实体或值。)  
**Problem solved:** it links language to what it is about. (它把语言同其所谈论之物连接起来。)  
**Why needed:** meaning is not only internal content; expressions can pick out objects. (意义不只是内部内容；表达可以选定对象。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing what a term, name, description, or sentence is about. (当分析术语、名称、描述或句子谈论什么时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Frege’s distinction between sense and reference is one of analytic philosophy’s foundational tools. “The morning star” and “the evening star” refer to the same planet, Venus, but they present it differently. Therefore, identity statements can be informative.  
  
This solves a problem in the philosophy of language: if meaning were only reference, then “the morning star is the evening star” would be no more informative than “Venus is Venus.” But it is informative because the senses differ.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Sense is the way a referent is presented; reference is what the expression refers to. (涵义是指称对象被呈现的方式；指称则是表达所指向的东西。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Sense (涵义; de: Sinn)** differs from **Reference (指称; de: Bedeutung)**. Two expressions can share reference while differing in sense. (两个表达可以具有相同指称，却具有不同涵义。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** sense/reference analysis shifts philosophical attention from ideas in the mind to public language, meaning, and logical structure. (涵义/指称分析把哲学注意力从心灵中的观念转向公共语言、意义和逻辑结构。)  
  
### 17. Proposition: The Problem of What Is True or False  
  
`Proposition (命题; la: propositio; en: proposition)`  
**Definition:** the content of a declarative claim that can be true or false. (一个可以为真或为假的陈述性主张内容。)  
**Problem solved:** it distinguishes the claim-content from the sentence, utterance, or psychological act. (它把主张内容同句子、话语行为或心理活动区分开来。)  
**Why needed:** different sentences in different languages can express the same claim. (不同语言中的不同句子可以表达同一个主张。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing truth, belief, assertion, inference, or logical relations. (当分析真理、信念、断言、推论或逻辑关系时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
A proposition is not the same as a sentence. “Snow is white” and “La neige est blanche” can express the same proposition in different languages. A proposition is also not the same as the mental act of believing it. Many people can believe the same proposition.  
  
This distinction allows analytic philosophy to separate language, thought, and truth.  
  
**Typical sentence:** A proposition is what is asserted, believed, denied, or evaluated as true or false. (命题是被断言、被相信、被否认或被评估为真假的东西。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Sentence (句子; en: sentence)** is a linguistic expression; **Proposition (命题; en: proposition)** is the truth-evaluable content expressed. (句子是语言表达；命题是被表达出来的可评估真假的内容。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** proposition-talk continues the Greek concern for **Logos (逻各斯; el: λόγος)** but formalizes it into truth-evaluable content. (命题话语延续希腊对 Logos 的关切，但把它形式化为可评估真假的内容。)  
  
### 18. Truth-Value and Truth-Conditions: The Problem of When a Claim Is True  
  
`Truth-Value (真值; en: truth-value)`  
**Definition:** the status of a proposition as true or false. (一个命题为真或为假的状态。)  
**Problem solved:** it makes logical evaluation possible. (它使逻辑评估成为可能。)  
**Why needed:** inference depends on how truth is preserved or transformed across propositions. (推论依赖真如何在命题之间被保存或转换。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing formal logic, semantics, assertion, or propositional structure. (当分析形式逻辑、语义学、断言或命题结构时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
`Truth-Condition (真值条件; en: truth-condition)`  
**Definition:** the condition under which a proposition would be true. (一个命题为真的条件。)  
**Problem solved:** it clarifies meaning by specifying what would make a claim true. (它通过说明什么会使一个主张为真来澄清意义。)  
**Why needed:** many philosophical claims become clearer when their truth-conditions are made explicit. (许多哲学主张在其真值条件被明确后会变得更清楚。)  
**How to use:** use it when asking what the world would have to be like for a sentence to be true. (当追问世界必须如何，一个句子才为真时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Truth-conditional analysis is one of analytic philosophy’s strongest tools. Instead of asking vaguely what a sentence “means,” one asks under what conditions it would be true.  
  
For example, “There is a cat on the mat” is true if and only if there is a cat on the mat. This may seem trivial, but the method becomes powerful when applied to modal, moral, mental, or metaphysical claims.  
  
**Typical sentence:** To give the truth-conditions of a sentence is to say what would make it true. (给出一个句子的真值条件，就是说明什么会使它为真。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Meaning (意义; en: meaning)** is broader than **Truth-Condition (真值条件; en: truth-condition)**. Some meanings involve use, force, affect, or context beyond truth-conditions. (意义宽于真值条件。有些意义涉及使用、语力、情感或语境，超出真值条件。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** truth-conditional semantics transforms truth from existential disclosure or regime of power into a formal relation between sentence, proposition, and world. (真值条件语义学把真理从存在开显或权力体制转化为句子、命题与世界之间的形式关系。)  
  
### 19. Possible Worlds: The Problem of Modal Thinking  
  
`Possible World (可能世界; en: possible world)`  
**Definition:** a way things could have been. (事物本来可能如此的一种方式。)  
**Problem solved:** it gives philosophy a tool for analyzing necessity, possibility, counterfactuals, and modal claims. (它为哲学提供分析必然性、可能性、反事实和模态主张的工具。)  
**Why needed:** many philosophical claims concern not only what is actual, but what could or must be the case. (许多哲学主张不仅关涉实际如此，也关涉可能如此或必然如此。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing modal logic, metaphysical possibility, necessity, identity, or counterfactual dependence. (当分析模态逻辑、形而上学可能性、必然性、同一性或反事实依赖时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Possible worlds are not necessarily parallel universes. In analytic philosophy, they often function as semantic or metaphysical tools. A proposition is necessary if true in all possible worlds. It is possible if true in at least one possible world.  
  
This makes modal claims precise.  
  
**Necessary (必然的; en: necessary):** true in all possible worlds. (在所有可能世界中为真。)  
  
**Possible (可能的; en: possible):** true in at least one possible world. (至少在一个可能世界中为真。)  
  
**Contingent (偶然的; en: contingent):** true in the actual world but false in some possible worlds. (在现实世界中为真，但在某些可能世界中为假。)  
  
**Typical sentence:** Possible worlds allow modal claims to be analyzed as claims about how things are across ways things could have been. (可能世界使模态主张能够被分析为关于事物在不同可能状态中如何成立的主张。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Actual World (现实世界; en: actual world)** is the world as it is; **Possible World (可能世界; en: possible world)** is a way the world could have been. (现实世界是世界实际所是；可能世界是世界本来可能所是的一种方式。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** possible-world semantics gives modern modal metaphysics a formal tool for old questions about necessity, essence, identity, and possibility. (可能世界语义学为现代模态形而上学提供形式工具，用以处理关于必然性、本质、同一性和可能性的古老问题。)  
  
### 20. Necessity, Possibility, and Contingency: The Problem of Modal Status  
  
`Necessity (必然性; la: necessitas; en: necessity)`  
**Definition:** the modal status of what could not have been otherwise. (不可能以其他方式存在或成立之物的模态地位。)  
**Problem solved:** it distinguishes strict inevitability from actuality. (它把严格不可另样性同现实性区分开来。)  
**Why needed:** something may be actual without being necessary. (某物可以是现实的，但并非必然的。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing what must be true. (当分析什么必须为真时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
`Possibility (可能性; la: possibilitas; en: possibility)`  
**Definition:** the modal status of what could be the case. (某事可能成立的模态地位。)  
**Problem solved:** it allows philosophy to distinguish impossibility from mere non-actuality. (它使哲学能够区分不可能性与单纯非现实性。)  
**Why needed:** something may not be actual but still be possible. (某物可以不现实，但仍然可能。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing what could be true or could exist. (当分析什么可能为真或可能存在时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
`Contingency (偶然性; la: contingentia; en: contingency)`  
**Definition:** the modal status of what is actual but could have been otherwise. (实际如此但本可不同的模态地位。)  
**Problem solved:** it prevents actuality from being mistaken for necessity. (它防止把现实性误认为必然性。)  
**Why needed:** many social, moral, and metaphysical claims depend on whether something is necessary or contingent. (许多社会、道德和形而上学主张取决于某物是必然的还是偶然的。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing whether a feature is essential, accidental, historical, or alterable. (当分析一个特征是本质的、偶然的、历史的还是可改变的时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
These modal terms are old, but analytic philosophy gives them new precision. A claim about possibility is not merely a claim about ignorance. A claim about necessity is not merely a claim about importance. Modal status concerns how things stand across possible ways the world could be.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Modal analysis asks whether a claim is merely actual, genuinely possible, strictly necessary, or contingent. (模态分析追问一个主张只是现实的、真正可能的、严格必然的，还是偶然的。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Actuality (现实性; de: Wirklichkeit; en: actuality)** means what is the case; **Necessity (必然性; en: necessity)** means what must be the case. (现实性意味着实际成立；必然性意味着必须成立。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** modal analysis connects analytic philosophy back to scholastic essence/existence debates and forward to contemporary metaphysics, philosophy of mind, and philosophy of language. (模态分析把分析哲学向后连接到经院本质/存在之争，向前连接到当代形而上学、心灵哲学和语言哲学。)  
  
### 21. Reference and Rigid Designation: The Problem of Naming Across Worlds  
  
`Rigid Designation (严格指示; en: rigid designation)`  
**Definition:** a term rigidly designates if it refers to the same object in every possible world in which that object exists. (如果一个术语在该对象存在的每个可能世界中都指称同一对象，它就是严格指示词。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains how names can refer across possible worlds without being equivalent to descriptions. (它解释名称如何能够跨可能世界指称，而不等同于描述。)  
**Why needed:** ordinary names often seem to pick out individuals directly rather than through a bundle of descriptive properties. (普通名称常似乎直接选定个体，而不是通过一组描述性属性。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing names, identity, necessity, and modal claims about objects. (当分析名称、同一性、必然性和关于对象的模态主张时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Rigid designation is central to Kripkean philosophy of language. The name “Aristotle” refers to Aristotle, even in possible worlds where Aristotle did not teach Alexander or did not write the *Metaphysics*. Descriptions may vary, but the name still picks out the same individual.  
  
This has deep metaphysical consequences. Some identity statements discovered empirically may be necessary if true, such as “water is H₂O,” under standard Kripkean analysis. The discovery is empirical; the identity, once fixed, is necessary.  
  
**Typical sentence:** A rigid designator refers to the same object across possible worlds, unlike descriptions that may pick out different objects under different conditions. (严格指示词跨可能世界指称同一对象，而描述在不同条件下可能选定不同对象。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Description (描述; en: description)** identifies by properties; **Rigid Designator (严格指示词; en: rigid designator)** picks out the same object across worlds. (描述通过属性识别；严格指示词跨世界选定同一对象。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** rigid designation challenges older descriptivist accounts of meaning and strengthens the link between language, necessity, and metaphysics. (严格指示挑战旧有的描述主义意义理论，并加强语言、必然性与形而上学之间的联系。)  
  
### 22. Supervenience: The Problem of Dependence without Reduction  
  
`Supervenience (随附性; en: supervenience)`  
**Definition:** a dependence relation in which there can be no difference in one set of properties without some difference in another set of properties. (一种依赖关系：若一组属性没有差异，另一组属性就不可能有差异。)  
**Problem solved:** it allows philosophers to express dependence without full reduction or identity. (它允许哲学家表达依赖关系，而不必诉诸完全还原或同一。)  
**Why needed:** many domains seem dependent on lower-level facts without being identical to them. (许多领域似乎依赖低层事实，却不等同于这些事实。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing relations between mental and physical, moral and natural, aesthetic and physical, or social and material properties. (当分析心理与物理、道德与自然、审美与物理，或社会与物质属性之间的关系时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Supervenience is a technical but useful tool. To say that mental properties supervene on physical properties is to say that there cannot be a mental difference without some physical difference. But this does not yet say that mental properties are identical to physical properties.  
  
This lets philosophers mark dependence while leaving reduction open.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Supervenience says that higher-level differences require lower-level differences, without automatically reducing the higher level to the lower level. (随附性表示高层差异需要低层差异，但不自动把高层还原为低层。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Identity (同一; en: identity)** says two things are the same; **Supervenience (随附性; en: supervenience)** says one level cannot vary without variation in another. (同一表示两个东西相同；随附性表示一个层级不能在另一个层级无变化时发生变化。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** supervenience becomes a key bridge concept in contemporary metaphysics, ethics, mind, and aesthetics. It provides a disciplined alternative to vague dependence-talk. (随附性成为当代形而上学、伦理学、心灵哲学和美学中的关键桥梁概念，为模糊的依赖话语提供纪律化替代。)  
  
### 23. Reduction: The Problem of Explaining One Domain by Another  
  
`Reduction (还原; en: reduction)`  
**Definition:** the explanation or identification of one domain in terms of a more basic domain. (用一个更基本领域来解释或识别另一个领域。)  
**Problem solved:** it clarifies whether apparently distinct phenomena are really fundamental. (它澄清表面上不同的现象是否真正基本。)  
**Why needed:** philosophy often asks whether mind, morality, meaning, or social facts can be explained by physical or natural facts. (哲学常追问心灵、道德、意义或社会事实是否能够由物理或自然事实解释。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing whether one kind of fact can be translated into, identified with, or explained by another kind of fact. (当分析一种事实是否能够被翻译为、等同于或由另一种事实解释时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Analytic reduction differs from phenomenological **Reduction (还原; de: Reduktion)**. Phenomenological reduction returns to structures of givenness. Analytic reduction asks whether one domain can be explained by another.  
  
For example, physicalism may try to reduce mental states to brain states. Moral naturalism may try to reduce moral properties to natural properties. Some theories reject reduction while accepting dependence.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Reduction asks whether one kind of fact can be fully explained in terms of another kind of fact. (还原追问一种事实是否能够完全由另一种事实解释。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Reduction (还原; en: reduction)** differs from **Elimination (取消; en: elimination)**. Reduction says the phenomenon is real but explainable in other terms; elimination says the supposed phenomenon does not exist as ordinarily conceived. (还原认为该现象真实但可由其他术语解释；取消则认为所谓现象并不存在于通常理解中。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** reduction becomes a central tool in philosophy of mind, science, ethics, and metaphysics. It also becomes a target for phenomenology, hermeneutics, and critical theory. (还原成为心灵哲学、科学哲学、伦理学和形而上学的核心工具，也成为现象学、解释学和批判理论的批判对象。)  
  
### 24. Naturalism: The Problem of Philosophy within the Natural World  
  
`Naturalism (自然主义; en: naturalism)`  
**Definition:** the view that philosophical explanation should be continuous with, constrained by, or compatible with natural science. (认为哲学解释应同自然科学连续、受其约束或与其兼容的观点。)  
**Problem solved:** it prevents philosophy from positing entities, faculties, or explanations disconnected from the natural world. (它防止哲学设定同自然世界脱节的实体、能力或解释。)  
**Why needed:** modern philosophy often seeks to avoid supernatural, purely speculative, or non-empirical excess. (现代哲学常试图避免超自然的、纯思辨的或非经验的过度设定。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing whether a theory fits with science, causality, biology, psychology, or physical explanation. (当分析一个理论是否符合科学、因果性、生物学、心理学或物理解释时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Naturalism has many forms. **Metaphysical Naturalism (形而上学自然主义; en: metaphysical naturalism)** says reality contains only natural entities or facts. **Methodological Naturalism (方法论自然主义; en: methodological naturalism)** says inquiry should use naturalistic methods. **Epistemological Naturalism (认识论自然主义; en: epistemological naturalism)** treats knowledge as continuous with empirical psychology or cognitive science.  
  
Naturalism is powerful, but it creates pressure. Can normativity, meaning, consciousness, logic, mathematics, and morality be fully naturalized?  
  
**Typical sentence:** Naturalism asks whether philosophical explanation can be made continuous with the natural sciences. (自然主义追问哲学解释是否能够同自然科学保持连续。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Naturalism (自然主义; en: naturalism)** differs from **Scientism (科学主义; en: scientism)**. Naturalism gives science philosophical authority; scientism overextends scientific method as the only legitimate form of understanding. (自然主义赋予科学以哲学权威；科学主义则把科学方法过度扩展为唯一合法理解形式。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** naturalism continues early modern mechanism and empiricism but becomes more sophisticated through logic, language, mind, and science. (自然主义延续近代机械论与经验论，但通过逻辑、语言、心灵和科学变得更复杂。)  
  
### 25. Normativity: The Problem of Ought, Reason, and Rule  
  
`Normativity (规范性; en: normativity)`  
**Definition:** the dimension of standards, reasons, obligations, correctness, or oughts. (标准、理由、义务、正确性或应当性维度。)  
**Problem solved:** it distinguishes what is the case from what ought to be, what is correct, or what one has reason to do. (它区分事实如何与应当如何、何者正确或人有什么理由去做。)  
**Why needed:** description alone does not explain obligation, justification, validity, or correctness. (单纯描述无法解释义务、证成、有效性或正确性。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing reasons, rules, moral claims, epistemic justification, meaning, or rational requirements. (当分析理由、规则、道德主张、认识论证成、意义或理性要求时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Normativity is one of the points where analytic philosophy resists simple naturalism. A belief may be caused by brain states, upbringing, or social pressure. But whether it is justified is a normative question. An action may be caused; whether it is right is another question. A sentence may be uttered; whether it is used correctly depends on norms.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Normativity concerns not merely what happens, but what is correct, justified, required, or permitted. (规范性关涉的不只是发生了什么，而是什么是正确的、被证成的、被要求的或被允许的。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Descriptive Claim (描述性主张; en: descriptive claim)** says what is the case; **Normative Claim (规范性主张; en: normative claim)** says what ought to be, what is justified, or what counts as correct. (描述性主张说明事实如何；规范性主张说明应当如何、什么被证成或什么算作正确。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** normativity reconnects analytic philosophy with Kantian questions of validity and practical reason, but in a language of reasons, rules, and justification. (规范性把分析哲学重新连接到康德关于有效性与实践理性的问题，但采用理由、规则和证成的语言。)  
  
### 26. The Tool-Map of Analytic Philosophy  
  
Use analytic vocabulary diagnostically. The central question is usually not “What historical force produced this?” or “How does this appear?” but “What exactly is being claimed, and does it work?”  
  
**If the text gives reasons for a thesis**, look for **Argument (论证; en: argument)**, **Premise (前提; en: premise)**, **Conclusion (结论; en: conclusion)**, and **Inference (推论; en: inference)**.  
(如果文本为一个论题给出理由，应寻找论证、前提、结论和推论问题。)  
  
**If the text evaluates logical structure**, look for **Validity (有效性; en: validity)**, **Soundness (可靠性; en: soundness)**, and **Entailment (蕴含; en: entailment)**.  
(如果文本评估逻辑结构，应寻找有效性、可靠性和蕴含问题。)  
  
**If the text clarifies a concept**, look for **Definition (定义; en: definition)**, **Necessary Condition (必要条件; en: necessary condition)**, **Sufficient Condition (充分条件; en: sufficient condition)**, and **Conceptual Analysis (概念分析; en: conceptual analysis)**.  
(如果文本澄清一个概念，应寻找定义、必要条件、充分条件和概念分析问题。)  
  
**If the text tests a theory with cases**, look for **Counterexample (反例; en: counterexample)**, **Thought Experiment (思想实验; en: thought experiment)**, and **Intuition (直觉; en: intuition)**.  
(如果文本用案例测试理论，应寻找反例、思想实验和直觉问题。)  
  
**If the text analyzes language**, look for **Use/Mention Distinction (使用/提及区分; en: use/mention distinction)**, **Sense (涵义; de: Sinn)**, **Reference (指称; de: Bedeutung/reference)**, **Proposition (命题; en: proposition)**, and **Truth-Condition (真值条件; en: truth-condition)**.  
(如果文本分析语言，应寻找使用/提及区分、涵义、指称、命题和真值条件问题。)  
  
**If the text analyzes possibility or necessity**, look for **Possible World (可能世界; en: possible world)**, **Necessity (必然性; en: necessity)**, **Possibility (可能性; en: possibility)**, **Contingency (偶然性; en: contingency)**, and **Rigid Designation (严格指示; en: rigid designation)**.  
(如果文本分析可能性或必然性，应寻找可能世界、必然性、可能性、偶然性和严格指示问题。)  
  
**If the text analyzes dependence between levels**, look for **Supervenience (随附性; en: supervenience)**, **Reduction (还原; en: reduction)**, and **Naturalism (自然主义; en: naturalism)**.  
(如果文本分析层级之间的依赖关系，应寻找随附性、还原和自然主义问题。)  
  
**If the text distinguishes fact from obligation or correctness**, look for **Normativity (规范性; en: normativity)**, **Reason (理由; en: reason)**, **Justification (证成; en: justification)**, and **Rule (规则; en: rule)**.  
(如果文本区分事实与义务或正确性，应寻找规范性、理由、证成和规则问题。)  
  
### 27. The Genealogical Point of Part 10  
  
Analytic philosophy transforms philosophical language into a technology of clarity. Greek philosophy asked for logos, form, being, and truth. Latin metaphysics stabilized essence, substance, law, and order. Early modern philosophy centered subject, representation, method, and certainty. Kant asked for conditions of possibility. German Idealism made concepts developmental. Marx and Nietzsche made concepts suspicious. Phenomenology returned to givenness. Heidegger reopened Being. Existentialism made freedom practical.  
  
Analytic philosophy asks philosophy to slow down and make its claims accountable.  
  
The guiding thesis is:  
  
**Analytic language turns philosophy into the disciplined control of claims: to understand a problem is to reconstruct its arguments, define its terms, test its conditions, identify its entailments, and examine the cases that would confirm or defeat it.**  
(分析哲学语言把哲学转化为对主张的纪律化控制：理解一个问题，就是重构其论证、定义其术语、检验其条件、识别其蕴含，并考察能够支持或击败它的案例。)  
  
This grammar is not opposed to depth. It is one way of protecting depth from vagueness. It can be combined with other traditions. A genealogical claim can be made clearer by specifying its thesis and evidence. A phenomenological description can be tested for conceptual overreach. A Heideggerian claim can be reconstructed into distinctions. An existentialist claim about freedom can be analyzed through conditions, counterexamples, and responsibility.  
  
The analytic question remains one of the strongest tools for philosophical reading:  
  
**What exactly is the claim, what supports it, what follows from it, and what would show it to be wrong?**  
(确切主张是什么？什么支持它？什么从中推出？什么会显示它是错误的？)  
  
## Part 11. Hermeneutics and Critical Theory: Interpretation, Society, Emancipation  
  
This chapter explains two related but distinct traditions: **Hermeneutics** and **Critical Theory**. Both reject the idea that knowledge is a neutral gaze at isolated objects. Hermeneutics asks how understanding is historically situated. Critical Theory asks how reason, society, and knowledge become entangled with domination. The shared problem is this: **understanding is never innocent, but neither can critique proceed without some claim to better understanding**. (理解从不中立无辜，但批判也不能不提出某种更好的理解要求。)  
  
The central vocabulary is **Hermeneutics**, **Interpretation**, **Understanding**, **Explanation**, **Hermeneutic Circle**, **Prejudice**, **Tradition**, **Horizon**, **Fusion of Horizons**, **Effective History**, **Critical Theory**, **Enlightenment**, **Instrumental Reason**, **Domination**, **Reification**, **Ideology**, **Emancipation**, **Communicative Rationality**, and **Immanent Critique**. **Hermeneutik**, **Hermeneutic Circle**, and **Horizontverschmelzung** name key hermeneutic structures, while instrumental reason, reification, and emancipation mark the critical-theory side of this vocabulary.  
  
The operational function of this chapter is exact: use hermeneutic vocabulary when the problem is **how meaning is understood across history, language, text, and tradition**; use critical-theoretical vocabulary when the problem is **how social reason becomes domination and how distorted social life can be criticized**. (当问题是意义如何跨越历史、语言、文本和传统而被理解时，应使用解释学词汇；当问题是社会理性如何成为支配，以及被扭曲的社会生活如何被批判时，应使用批判理论词汇。)  
  
### 1. The Problem-Situation: Understanding Is Historical  
  
Analytic philosophy asks: what exactly is the argument? Phenomenology asks: how is something given? Heidegger asks: what mode of Being is presupposed? Existentialism asks: how does finite freedom choose? Hermeneutics asks a different question:  
  
**How is understanding possible when every interpreter already belongs to a language, history, tradition, and horizon?**  
(当每个解释者都已经属于一种语言、历史、传统和视域时，理解如何可能？)  
  
This question rejects two simplifications.  
  
First, understanding is not mechanical decoding. A text, law, ritual, artwork, institution, or action does not simply contain a fixed meaning waiting to be extracted. Meaning appears through interpretation.  
  
Second, interpretation is not arbitrary projection. The interpreter is not free to make anything mean anything. The text, tradition, language, context, and subject matter resist arbitrary reading.  
  
Hermeneutics therefore lives in a tension:  
  
**Meaning is historically mediated, but not infinitely plastic.**  
(意义是历史地被中介的，但并非无限可塑。)  
  
Critical Theory adds another pressure:  
  
**What if the historical forms through which understanding occurs are themselves distorted by domination?**  
(如果理解得以发生的历史形式本身已经被支配扭曲，又该如何？)  
  
This is where hermeneutics and critical theory meet. Hermeneutics emphasizes situated understanding. Critical Theory emphasizes distorted social conditions and the need for emancipation.  
  
### 2. Hermeneutics: The Problem of Understanding Meaning  
  
`Hermeneutics (解释学/阐释学; el: ἑρμηνεύειν; de: Hermeneutik)`  
**Definition:** the theory and practice of interpretation, especially of texts, actions, traditions, and historically mediated meaning. (关于解释的理论与实践，尤其涉及文本、行动、传统和历史中介的意义。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains how meaning can be understood when it is not immediately transparent. (它解释当意义并非直接透明时，意义如何能够被理解。)  
**Why needed:** human meanings are embedded in language, context, history, genre, practice, and tradition. (人类意义嵌入语言、语境、历史、文类、实践和传统之中。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing interpretation across distance: textual, historical, cultural, legal, religious, or existential. (当分析跨越距离的解释时，应使用这一概念：文本距离、历史距离、文化距离、法律距离、宗教距离或生存距离。)  
  
Hermeneutics begins from the fact that meaning is mediated. A legal clause, a poem, a philosophical text, a religious scripture, or a political speech cannot be understood by translating words one by one. Meaning depends on use, genre, historical background, question-context, and interpretive expectation.  
  
This makes hermeneutics useful beyond literary study. Law, theology, history, social science, psychoanalysis, political theory, and philosophy all require interpretation.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Hermeneutics asks how meaning becomes understandable across historical, linguistic, and contextual distance. (解释学追问意义如何跨越历史、语言和语境距离而变得可理解。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Hermeneutics (解释学; de: Hermeneutik)** differs from **Decoding (解码; en: decoding)**. Decoding treats meaning as already fixed in signs; hermeneutics treats meaning as historically and contextually disclosed. (解码把意义视为已经固定在符号中；解释学把意义视为历史和语境中被开显的东西。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** hermeneutics moves interpretation from a technical art of reading difficult texts to a general theory of human understanding. (解释学从阅读困难文本的技术艺术，转变为关于人类理解的一般理论。)  
  
### 3. Interpretation: The Problem of Meaning as Mediated  
  
`Interpretation (解释; la: interpretatio; de: Auslegung/Interpretation)`  
**Definition:** the act of articulating meaning by relating parts, whole, context, language, and question. (通过关联部分、整体、语境、语言和问题来阐明意义的活动。)  
**Problem solved:** it makes explicit the meaning that is implicit, obscure, contested, or historically distant. (它使隐含的、晦暗的、有争议的或历史上遥远的意义变得明确。)  
**Why needed:** meaning is rarely self-contained; it usually requires mediation through context and understanding. (意义很少自足；它通常需要通过语境和理解来中介。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing how a text, action, institution, or event is made intelligible. (当分析文本、行动、制度或事件如何成为可理解之物时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Interpretation is not an optional supplement added after meaning is found. It is often the way meaning becomes accessible at all. The interpreter does not simply reproduce meaning. The interpreter enters into a relation with the text or object.  
  
This does not mean interpretation is arbitrary. A good interpretation is answerable to the thing interpreted. It must explain details, fit the whole, respect genre, handle objections, and disclose what the object is about.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Interpretation is the disciplined mediation through which meaning becomes articulate. (解释是意义变得可阐明的有规训中介。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Interpretation (解释; de: Auslegung)** differs from **Projection (投射; de: Projektion)**. Interpretation is answerable to the text or phenomenon; projection imposes meaning without sufficient responsiveness. (解释必须回应文本或现象；投射则在缺乏充分回应的情况下强加意义。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** interpretation becomes a basic condition of human understanding, not merely a method for special texts. (解释成为人类理解的基本条件，而不只是特殊文本的方法。)  
  
### 4. Understanding and Explanation: The Problem of Human Meaning versus Causal Account  
  
`Understanding (理解; de: Verstehen)`  
**Definition:** grasping meaning from within a context of action, language, practice, or life. (从行动、语言、实践或生活的语境内部把握意义。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains how human actions and texts can be made intelligible as meaningful rather than merely caused. (它解释人类行动和文本如何作为有意义之物而不只是作为被导致之物被理解。)  
**Why needed:** human actions are not fully understood by causal description alone. (仅靠因果描述无法充分理解人类行动。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing meaning, intention, practice, norm, text, or historical life. (当分析意义、意图、实践、规范、文本或历史生活时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
`Explanation (说明/解释; de: Erklären)`  
**Definition:** giving causal, functional, structural, or law-like account of why something occurs. (对某事为何发生给出因果的、功能的、结构的或规律式说明。)  
**Problem solved:** it identifies causes, mechanisms, structures, or conditions. (它识别原因、机制、结构或条件。)  
**Why needed:** not all understanding can remain at the level of meaning; some phenomena require causal or structural account. (并非所有理解都能停留在意义层面；有些现象需要因果或结构说明。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing mechanisms, causes, social structures, or objective conditions. (当分析机制、原因、社会结构或客观条件时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
The distinction between **Verstehen** and **Erklären** is central. To understand why someone raised a hand in a classroom, one may need meaning: asking a question, voting, greeting, surrendering, stretching. The same physical movement can have different meanings. A purely causal account of muscle movement is insufficient.  
  
But explanation also matters. A social practice may need both meaning and structure. A worker’s action may be understood from within their intention, but also explained through class, institution, law, and economic compulsion.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Understanding grasps meaning from within; explanation identifies causes or structures from without. (理解从内部把握意义；说明从外部识别原因或结构。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Understanding (理解; de: Verstehen)** is not subjective empathy alone; **Explanation (说明; de: Erklären)** is not automatically deeper. They answer different questions. (理解并不只是主观移情；说明也不自动更深。二者回答不同问题。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** this distinction becomes central for debates about human sciences, social sciences, psychoanalysis, law, anthropology, and history. (这一区分成为关于人文科学、社会科学、精神分析、法律、人类学和历史学争论的核心。)  
  
### 5. Hermeneutic Circle: The Problem of Part and Whole  
  
`Hermeneutic Circle (解释学循环; de: hermeneutischer Zirkel)`  
**Definition:** the structure by which the parts of a text or phenomenon are understood through the whole, while the whole is understood through the parts. (文本或现象的部分通过整体被理解，而整体又通过部分被理解的结构。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains why understanding develops circularly rather than linearly. (它解释为什么理解以循环方式而非线性方式发展。)  
**Why needed:** no part has full meaning in isolation, and no whole is available without interpreting parts. (任何部分都不能孤立地拥有充分意义，而整体也无法在不解释部分的情况下获得。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing how interpretation revises itself through movement between detail and whole. (当分析解释如何在细节与整体之间往返并修订自身时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
The hermeneutic circle is not a logical fallacy. It is a structure of understanding. A sentence depends on the paragraph. A paragraph depends on the whole work. The whole work is understood only by reading sentences and paragraphs. Understanding therefore moves back and forth.  
  
This applies beyond texts. A human action is understood through a life; a life through actions. A legal provision is understood through a legal system; the system through provisions. A historical event is understood through an epoch; the epoch through events.  
  
**Typical sentence:** The hermeneutic circle is not vicious circularity, but the movement through which understanding becomes more adequate. (解释学循环不是恶性循环，而是理解变得更充分的运动。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Vicious Circle (恶性循环; en: vicious circle)** invalidly assumes what it must prove; **Hermeneutic Circle (解释学循环; de: hermeneutischer Zirkel)** describes the necessary interplay of part and whole in understanding. (恶性循环非法预设其必须证明之物；解释学循环描述理解中部分与整体的必要互动。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** the hermeneutic circle transforms method. Understanding is not a neutral procedure applied from outside; it is a self-correcting participation in meaning. (解释学循环改造了方法概念。理解不是从外部应用的中立程序，而是对意义的自我修正性参与。)  
  
### 6. Prejudice: The Problem of Prior Understanding  
  
`Prejudice (前见; de: Vorurteil)`  
**Definition:** a prior judgment, anticipation, or orientation that shapes understanding before explicit reflection. (在明确反思之前塑造理解的先行判断、期待或取向。)  
**Problem solved:** it challenges the Enlightenment assumption that all prejudice is mere error. (它挑战启蒙思想中把一切前见都视为错误的假设。)  
**Why needed:** no interpreter begins from nowhere; understanding always starts from prior commitments and expectations. (没有解释者从无处开始；理解总是从先行承诺和期待开始。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing the background assumptions that make interpretation possible and risky. (当分析使解释既可能又有风险的背景假设时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
In ordinary language, prejudice is usually negative. In Gadamer’s hermeneutics, **prejudice** has a broader technical sense. It means prior judgment. Some prejudices distort understanding. Others make understanding possible. A reader cannot understand anything without anticipations of meaning.  
  
The task is not to eliminate all prejudices, which is impossible. The task is to bring them into play, test them, revise them, and expose false ones.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Prejudice is not always error; it is the prior orientation from which understanding begins. (前见并不总是错误；它是理解由之开始的先行取向。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Prejudice (前见; de: Vorurteil)** differs from **Bias (偏见; en: bias)** in the narrow negative sense. Bias distorts; prejudice in the hermeneutic sense can also enable understanding. (前见不同于狭义负面的偏见。偏见会扭曲；解释学意义上的前见也可以使理解成为可能。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** hermeneutics turns the critique of prejudice against itself. The demand to be free of all prejudice may itself be a prejudice of abstract reason. (解释学把对前见的批判反转回来：要求摆脱一切前见本身可能就是抽象理性的前见。)  
  
### 7. Tradition: The Problem of Historical Belonging  
  
`Tradition (传统; la: traditio; de: Überlieferung/Tradition)`  
**Definition:** the historically transmitted field of meanings, practices, texts, norms, and questions within which understanding occurs. (理解在其中发生的、历史传递下来的意义、实践、文本、规范和问题领域。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains why understanding is inherited rather than invented from nothing. (它解释为什么理解是被继承的，而不是从无中发明的。)  
**Why needed:** language, concepts, institutions, and questions come to the interpreter through history. (语言、概念、制度和问题通过历史传递给解释者。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing inherited meanings, authority, continuity, transmission, or historical formation of understanding. (当分析继承意义、权威、连续性、传递或理解的历史形成时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Tradition is not merely the past. It is the past as active in the present. One does not stand outside tradition and inspect it neutrally. One belongs to it before criticizing it.  
  
This does not mean tradition must be obeyed. Hermeneutics does not simply defend conservatism. It means that critique itself uses inherited language, concepts, and questions. Even rebellion is historically mediated.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Tradition is not a dead past behind us, but the living transmission through which questions and meanings reach us. (传统不是身后的死去过去，而是问题与意义借以抵达我们的活的传递。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Tradition (传统; de: Überlieferung)** differs from **Traditionalism (传统主义; en: traditionalism)**. Tradition names historical transmission; traditionalism demands obedience to inherited forms. (传统命名历史传递；传统主义要求服从继承形式。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** tradition transforms the modern ideal of autonomous reason. Reason does not begin from pure self-grounding; it works within inherited horizons. (传统改造现代自主理性的理想。理性不是从纯粹自我奠基开始，而是在继承的视域中工作。)  
  
### 8. Horizon: The Problem of Situated Possibility  
  
`Horizon (视域; de: Horizont)`  
**Definition:** the historically situated field of possible meanings, questions, expectations, and intelligibility. (由历史处境规定的可能意义、问题、期待和可理解性场域。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains why interpretation is shaped by what can be seen, asked, or expected from a given standpoint. (它解释解释为什么受制于从某一立足点能够看见、提出或期待的东西。)  
**Why needed:** no interpreter sees everything; every understanding has limits and openings. (没有解释者能看见一切；每种理解都有其限度与开放性。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing the background field that determines what meanings are available. (当分析决定哪些意义可用的背景场域时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
A horizon is not a wall. It limits and opens. It marks what can appear from a standpoint, while also moving as one moves. Understanding requires awareness of one’s horizon and encounter with another horizon.  
  
This concept links phenomenology and hermeneutics. In phenomenology, horizon names the background of possible appearances. In hermeneutics, it names the historical field of possible understanding.  
  
**Typical sentence:** A horizon is the field within which something can appear as meaningful from a historically situated standpoint. (视域是某物能够从一个历史处境化立足点显现为有意义之物的场域。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Perspective (视角; de: Perspektive)** often emphasizes standpoint; **Horizon (视域; de: Horizont)** emphasizes the wider field of possible meaning opened by that standpoint. (视角强调立足点；视域强调由该立足点开启的更广阔可能意义场。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** horizon becomes a bridge between phenomenological givenness and historical interpretation. (视域成为现象学给予性与历史解释之间的桥梁。)  
  
### 9. Fusion of Horizons: The Problem of Understanding across Difference  
  
`Fusion of Horizons (视域融合; de: Horizontverschmelzung)`  
**Definition:** the event in which interpreter and text, present and past, or different horizons enter into a transformed understanding. (解释者与文本、现在与过去，或不同视域进入一种被转化的理解事件。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains how understanding across historical distance is possible without erasing difference. (它解释跨越历史距离的理解如何可能，同时不抹除差异。)  
**Why needed:** interpretation cannot simply reproduce the past, nor can it merely impose the present. (解释不能简单复制过去，也不能只是把现在强加给过去。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing how encounter with another horizon changes the interpreter’s own horizon. (当分析同另一视域的遭遇如何改变解释者自身视域时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Fusion of horizons does not mean total agreement. It means that understanding occurs when the interpreter’s horizon is enlarged through encounter with what is other. The text asks questions of the interpreter; the interpreter brings questions to the text. Meaning emerges through this encounter.  
  
This is why good interpretation can transform the interpreter. One does not merely acquire information. One’s own assumptions can be revised.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Fusion of horizons occurs when understanding transforms both the meaning of the text for us and our own horizon of questioning. (当理解同时转化文本对我们的意义和我们自身的提问视域时，视域融合就发生了。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Assimilation (同化; en: assimilation)** absorbs the other into one’s own framework; **Fusion of Horizons (视域融合; de: Horizontverschmelzung)** transforms understanding through encounter with difference. (同化把他者吸收到自身框架中；视域融合通过同差异的遭遇转化理解。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** this concept gives hermeneutics an anti-objectivist but non-arbitrary account of historical understanding. (这一概念为解释学提供一种反客观主义但非任意主义的历史理解说明。)  
  
### 10. Effective History: The Problem of History Working through Us  
  
`Effective History (效果历史; de: Wirkungsgeschichte)`  
**Definition:** the ongoing effect of history on present understanding. (历史对当下理解的持续作用。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains why the past is not merely an object of study but an active force in interpretation. (它解释为什么过去不只是研究对象，而是解释中的活动力量。)  
**Why needed:** interpreters are shaped by histories they do not fully control or see. (解释者被其无法完全控制或看见的历史所塑造。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing how inherited meanings, institutions, texts, and events continue to shape present understanding. (当分析继承意义、制度、文本和事件如何继续塑造当下理解时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Effective history means that the interpreter is never outside history. Even the attempt to be objective occurs within a history of objectivity. Even critique has a history.  
  
This concept is close to genealogy but not identical. Genealogy often emphasizes contingency, struggle, and power. Effective history emphasizes the ongoing influence of tradition on understanding.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Effective history means that history works through the interpreter before the interpreter works on history. (效果历史意味着在解释者处理历史之前，历史已经通过解释者发生作用。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Historical Object (历史对象; en: historical object)** is something studied; **Effective History (效果历史; de: Wirkungsgeschichte)** is history as active in the conditions of study. (历史对象是被研究的东西；效果历史则是作为研究条件而发挥作用的历史。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** effective history deepens the critique of detached neutrality. The observer is always already historically affected. (效果历史深化了对脱离式中立性的批判。观察者总是已经被历史影响。)  
  
### 11. Critical Theory: The Problem of Reason Turned into Domination  
  
`Critical Theory (批判理论; de: Kritische Theorie)`  
**Definition:** a form of social philosophy that analyzes domination, ideology, and distorted reason in order to make emancipation possible. (一种社会哲学，它分析支配、意识形态和被扭曲的理性，以使解放成为可能。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains why modern reason and society can produce domination while claiming progress. (它解释现代性中的理性与社会为何会在声称进步的同时生产支配。)  
**Why needed:** social critique must examine not only false beliefs, but the institutions and rationalities that reproduce unfreedom. (社会批判必须考察的不只是虚假信念，还包括再生产不自由的制度和理性形式。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing domination, ideology, capitalism, culture industry, instrumental reason, social pathology, or emancipation. (当分析支配、意识形态、资本主义、文化工业、工具理性、社会病理或解放时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Critical Theory inherits Marx but does not simply repeat economic determinism. It asks how domination appears in culture, reason, science, technology, law, family, media, and everyday life. It also inherits Kant and Hegel: critique must be rational, but reason itself must be criticized.  
  
This produces a difficult problem:  
  
**How can reason criticize domination if reason itself has become a vehicle of domination?**  
(如果理性本身已经成为支配工具，理性如何还能批判支配？)  
  
Critical Theory lives inside this tension.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Critical Theory asks how modern society can be rationalized and yet remain unfree. (批判理论追问现代社会如何能够被理性化却仍然不自由。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Traditional Theory (传统理论; de: traditionelle Theorie)** seeks neutral explanation; **Critical Theory (批判理论; de: Kritische Theorie)** seeks to understand society in relation to domination and emancipation. (传统理论寻求中立说明；批判理论则在支配与解放的关系中理解社会。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** critique moves from Kant’s limits of reason and Marx’s critique of capitalism toward a broader diagnosis of modern rationalized society. (批判从康德对理性限度的考察和马克思对资本主义的批判，转向对现代理性化社会的更广泛诊断。)  
  
### 12. Enlightenment: The Problem of Liberation and Control  
  
`Enlightenment (启蒙; de: Aufklärung; fr: Lumières)`  
**Definition:** the historical project of liberating human beings through reason, critique, science, and autonomy. (通过理性、批判、科学和自主性解放人类的历史工程。)  
**Problem solved:** it challenges myth, superstition, arbitrary authority, and inherited domination. (它挑战神话、迷信、任意权威和继承支配。)  
**Why needed:** emancipation requires the capacity to question authority and justify norms rationally. (解放需要质疑权威并理性证成规范的能力。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing modernity’s promise of liberation through reason and its possible reversal into domination. (当分析现代性通过理性实现解放的承诺及其可能反转为支配时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Critical Theory does not simply reject the Enlightenment. It diagnoses its dialectic. Enlightenment fights myth by making the world calculable and controllable. But this very drive toward control can become domination over nature, society, and human beings.  
  
The danger is not reason as such. The danger is reason reduced to control.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Enlightenment promises liberation through reason, but it can turn reason into a system of control. (启蒙承诺通过理性实现解放，但它也可能把理性转化为控制系统。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Enlightenment (启蒙; de: Aufklärung)** differs from **Instrumental Rationalization (工具理性化; de: instrumentelle Rationalisierung)**. Enlightenment includes critique and autonomy; instrumental rationalization reduces reason to efficient control. (启蒙包含批判和自主性；工具理性化把理性缩减为有效控制。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** Critical Theory turns Enlightenment against itself: the project of liberation must criticize its own domination-producing tendencies. (批判理论使启蒙反思自身：解放工程必须批判自身生产支配的倾向。)  
  
### 13. Instrumental Reason: The Problem of Means without Ends  
  
`Instrumental Reason (工具理性; de: instrumentelle Vernunft)`  
**Definition:** reason reduced to the efficient selection of means for given ends. (被缩减为为既定目的选择有效手段的理性。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains how rationality can become technically effective while normatively empty. (它解释理性如何能够在技术上有效却在规范上空洞。)  
**Why needed:** modern domination often operates through calculation, administration, efficiency, and control rather than open irrationality. (现代支配常通过计算、管理、效率和控制运作，而不是通过公开非理性运作。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing bureaucratic control, technological rationality, optimization, management, or the reduction of values to utility. (当分析官僚控制、技术理性、优化、管理或价值被化约为效用时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Instrumental reason does not ask whether the end is good. It asks how to achieve it efficiently. This makes it powerful and dangerous. It can build hospitals, coordinate transport, optimize production, and organize knowledge. It can also administer domination, surveillance, propaganda, and destruction.  
  
The critical problem is not that means are irrelevant. The problem is the collapse of reason into means-calculation.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Instrumental reason asks how to achieve an end efficiently, but not whether the end is worthy. (工具理性追问如何有效实现目的，却不追问该目的是否值得。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Instrumental Reason (工具理性; de: instrumentelle Vernunft)** differs from **Practical Reason (实践理性; de: praktische Vernunft)**. Practical reason asks what ought to be done; instrumental reason asks how to do what has already been chosen. (实践理性追问应当做什么；工具理性追问如何实现已经被选择的目的。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** instrumental reason links Critical Theory with Heidegger’s **Gestell (集置; de: Gestell)**. Both diagnose modernity as a mode in which beings appear primarily through availability, calculation, and control. (工具理性把批判理论同海德格尔的集置连接起来。二者都诊断现代性把存在者主要作为可用、可计算和可控制之物来显现。)  
  
### 14. Domination: The Problem of Structured Unfreedom  
  
`Domination (支配; de: Herrschaft)`  
**Definition:** a structured relation in which some persons, groups, systems, or rationalities control, constrain, or shape others in ways that block autonomy or flourishing. (某些个人、群体、系统或理性形式控制、限制或塑造他者，从而阻碍自主性或良好生活的结构性关系。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains unfreedom as systemic rather than merely personal. (它把不自由解释为系统性的，而不只是个人性的。)  
**Why needed:** modern power often operates through institutions, norms, markets, media, and rationalized administration. (现代权力常通过制度、规范、市场、媒体和理性化管理运作。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing structured inequality, coercion, dependency, manipulation, or social pathology. (当分析结构性不平等、强制、依赖、操控或社会病理时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Domination is not reducible to visible violence. It can appear as normal work, consumption, entertainment, education, law, management, expertise, or cultural aspiration. Critical Theory asks how domination becomes ordinary.  
  
This is where Critical Theory differs from simple moral criticism. It does not only say that some people behave badly. It examines forms of life that reproduce unfreedom even when individuals think they are acting freely.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Domination is most powerful when it appears as normal social reality rather than explicit coercion. (当支配表现为正常社会现实而非明确强制时，它最有力量。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Power (权力; de: Macht)** is the capacity to affect action; **Domination (支配; de: Herrschaft)** is a structured and often asymmetrical form of power that blocks freedom. (权力是影响行动的能力；支配则是一种结构化且常常不对称的权力形式，它阻碍自由。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** domination broadens Marx’s critique of exploitation into a wider analysis of culture, reason, institutions, and subject formation. (支配把马克思对剥削的批判扩展为对文化、理性、制度和主体形成的更广泛分析。)  
  
### 15. Reification: The Problem of Relations Becoming Things  
  
`Reification (物化; de: Verdinglichung)`  
**Definition:** the process by which human relations, activities, or social forms appear as thing-like, natural, fixed, and independent of human practice. (人类关系、活动或社会形式表现为物一样的、自然的、固定的、独立于人类实践的东西的过程。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains how historically produced relations come to appear as objective things. (它解释历史生产出来的关系如何显得像客观物。)  
**Why needed:** capitalist and bureaucratic societies often transform living relations into calculable, exchangeable, administrable objects. (资本主义和官僚制社会常把活的关系转化为可计算、可交换、可管理的对象。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing objectification, commodification, bureaucratic abstraction, or the freezing of social relations into thing-forms. (当分析对象化、商品化、官僚抽象或社会关系冻结为物形式时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Reification develops Marx’s commodity fetishism. In reified society, not only commodities but also labor, time, personality, knowledge, culture, and relationships become thing-like. The worker becomes labor-power. The student becomes a metric. The patient becomes a case. The citizen becomes data.  
  
Reification is not merely a mistaken idea. It is a social form that makes the mistake real in practice.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Reification occurs when relations between people appear as fixed properties of things or systems. (当人与人之间的关系表现为物或系统的固定属性时，物化就发生了。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Objectification (对象化; de: Vergegenständlichung)** can be a normal process of making activity objective; **Reification (物化; de: Verdinglichung)** is objectification hardened into alien thinghood. (对象化可以是使活动客观化的正常过程；物化则是硬化为异己物性的对象化。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** reification connects Marx, Lukács, Critical Theory, and later critiques of bureaucracy, consumer culture, quantification, and digital capitalism. (物化连接马克思、卢卡奇、批判理论，以及后来对官僚制、消费文化、量化和数字资本主义的批判。)  
  
### 16. Ideology: The Problem of Distorted Social Consciousness  
  
`Ideology (意识形态; de: Ideologie)`  
**Definition:** a system of meanings, representations, and assumptions that legitimates or conceals domination. (一种使支配合法化或遮蔽支配的意义、表象和假设系统。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains how social domination can reproduce itself through belief, culture, common sense, and normality. (它解释社会支配如何通过信念、文化、常识和正常性再生产自身。)  
**Why needed:** domination does not persist by force alone; it also requires interpretation of reality. (支配并不只靠强力维持；它还需要对现实的解释。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing false universality, naturalization, legitimation, common sense, or distorted recognition. (当分析虚假普遍性、自然化、合法化、常识或扭曲承认时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
**Usage layers:**  
1. **Marxian use (马克思式用法):** **ideology** names a form of consciousness, representation, or social appearance that presents historically produced relations as natural, universal, or necessary. (意识形态指一种意识、表象或社会显现形式，它把历史地生产出来的关系呈现为自然的、普遍的或必然的。)  
  
2. **Critical-theory reception use (批判理论接受史用法):** in critical theory, ideology is often analyzed as distorted social consciousness reproduced through culture, institutions, media, reason, authority, or everyday life. (在批判理论中，意识形态常被分析为通过文化、制度、媒介、理性、权威或日常生活再生产的扭曲社会意识。)  
  
3. **Contemporary transferable use (当代理论泛用法):** in cultural studies, law, technology studies, and political theory, ideology may refer to the frameworks that organize common sense, visibility, legitimacy, aspiration, and consent. (在文化研究、法学、技术研究和政治理论中，意识形态可指组织常识、可见性、合法性、欲望和同意的框架。)  
  
**Transfer rule:** use **ideology** when a representation helps reproduce social relations by making them appear natural, neutral, inevitable, or desirable. Do not use it merely as a synonym for “opinion” or “belief.” (转用规则：当某种表象通过把社会关系呈现为自然、中立、不可避免或值得欲求而帮助再生产这些关系时，才使用 ideology。不要把它简单当成 opinion 或 belief 的同义词。)  
  
**Misuse warning:** **Ideology** does not simply mean “false idea.” It concerns the social function of representation. (Ideology 不只是“错误观念”，而关涉表象的社会功能。)  
  
Critical Theory inherits Marx’s concept of ideology but expands it. Ideology is not only a ruling-class doctrine. It can be embedded in entertainment, family norms, consumer desires, expertise, education, and self-understanding.  
  
A society may teach people to experience domination as freedom: choosing between commodities, optimizing oneself for labor markets, identifying with imposed standards, or accepting inequality as merit.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Ideology makes domination intelligible as normal, natural, deserved, or free. (意识形态使支配显得正常、自然、应得或自由。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **False Belief (虚假信念; en: false belief)** is an incorrect proposition; **Ideology (意识形态; de: Ideologie)** is a socially organized pattern of distorted intelligibility. (虚假信念是错误命题；意识形态是社会组织起来的扭曲可理解性模式。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** ideology critique prepares later discourse analysis and Foucault’s power/knowledge, but differs from Foucault because it often retains a stronger contrast between distorted and emancipated understanding. (意识形态批判为后来的话语分析和福柯的权力/知识做准备，但它不同于福柯，因为它通常保留更强的扭曲理解与解放性理解之间的对照。)  
  
### 17. Culture Industry: The Problem of Manufactured Consciousness  
  
`Culture Industry (文化工业; de: Kulturindustrie)`  
**Definition:** the mass production and standardization of culture under capitalist conditions. (资本主义条件下文化的大规模生产与标准化。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains how entertainment and culture can reproduce conformity. (它解释娱乐和文化如何能够再生产从众。)  
**Why needed:** domination in modern societies often works through pleasure, distraction, consumption, and identification rather than direct censorship alone. (现代社会中的支配常通过快感、分散、消费和认同运作，而不只是通过直接审查。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing mass media, entertainment, advertising, consumer desire, standardization, or pseudo-individuality. (当分析大众媒体、娱乐、广告、消费欲望、标准化或伪个性时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
The culture industry thesis does not simply say popular culture is bad. It says culture becomes industrially organized in ways that standardize perception, desire, and expectation. Even individuality can be sold as a standardized product.  
  
This concept remains useful for analyzing algorithmic entertainment, influencer culture, branding, platform attention, and self-commodification.  
  
**Typical sentence:** The culture industry sells individuality in standardized forms. (文化工业以标准化形式出售个性。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Culture (文化; la: cultura; de: Kultur)** can involve symbolic formation, memory, and creativity; **Culture Industry (文化工业; de: Kulturindustrie)** names culture organized as mass production and consumption. (文化可以涉及符号形成、记忆和创造；文化工业命名作为大规模生产与消费而被组织的文化。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** culture becomes a terrain of domination, not merely a realm of refinement or expression. (文化成为支配场域，而不只是教养或表达领域。)  
  
### 18. Emancipation: The Problem of Freedom from Distorted Conditions  
  
`Emancipation (解放; la: emancipatio; de: Emanzipation)`  
**Definition:** liberation from social, ideological, economic, or communicative conditions that block autonomy and flourishing. (从阻碍自主性与良好生活的社会、意识形态、经济或交往条件中解放出来。)  
**Problem solved:** it gives critique a practical orientation beyond description. (它为批判提供超出描述的实践取向。)  
**Why needed:** critical theory does not only interpret domination; it seeks the possibility of overcoming it. (批判理论不只是解释支配；它寻求克服支配的可能性。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing liberation, autonomy, recognition, social transformation, or undistorted communication. (当分析解放、自主性、承认、社会转化或未受扭曲的交往时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Emancipation is not simple individual self-expression. It requires transformation of conditions. A person cannot become fully free if social structures systematically produce dependency, humiliation, misrecognition, poverty, or ideological distortion.  
  
This is why Critical Theory keeps returning to society as a whole. Freedom is not merely inner attitude. It is socially mediated.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Emancipation means transforming the conditions that make unfreedom appear normal. (解放意味着转化那些使不自由显得正常的条件。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Liberation (释放/解放; en: liberation)** can mean removal of constraint; **Emancipation (解放; de: Emanzipation)** in critical theory often means reflective and social freedom from domination. (Liberation 可以指约束的解除；批判理论中的 emancipation 常指从支配中获得反思性的社会自由。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** emancipation links Kantian autonomy, Hegelian recognition, Marxian liberation, and modern social critique. (解放连接康德式自主性、黑格尔式承认、马克思式解放和现代社会批判。)  
  
### 19. Communicative Rationality: The Problem of Reason beyond Instrumentality  
  
`Communicative Rationality (交往理性; de: kommunikative Rationalität)`  
**Definition:** reason oriented toward mutual understanding, justification, and agreement rather than control or success alone. (一种朝向相互理解、证成和同意的理性，而非只朝向控制或成功。)  
**Problem solved:** it offers a model of reason that is not reducible to instrumental calculation. (它提供一种不能被化约为工具计算的理性模型。)  
**Why needed:** if reason is only instrumental, critique loses the rational basis for criticizing domination. (如果理性只是工具性的，批判就失去批判支配的理性基础。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing discourse, justification, democratic deliberation, validity claims, or undistorted communication. (当分析话语、证成、民主审议、有效性要求或未受扭曲的交往时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Habermas responds to earlier Critical Theory by trying to recover a non-instrumental form of reason. In communication, speakers raise validity claims: truth, rightness, sincerity, and intelligibility. These claims can be challenged and defended.  
  
This gives critique a normative ground. Domination can be criticized when it blocks free and equal participation in communication.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Communicative rationality is reason oriented toward understanding rather than control. (交往理性是朝向理解而非控制的理性。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Instrumental Reason (工具理性; de: instrumentelle Vernunft)** seeks efficient success; **Communicative Rationality (交往理性; de: kommunikative Rationalität)** seeks justifiable understanding. (工具理性追求有效成功；交往理性追求可证成的理解。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** communicative rationality tries to rescue Enlightenment reason from its reduction to domination. (交往理性试图从理性被化约为支配的命运中拯救启蒙理性。)  
  
### 20. Immanent Critique: The Problem of Criticizing from Within  
  
`Immanent Critique (内在批判; de: immanente Kritik)`  
**Definition:** critique that evaluates a social form, theory, or institution by its own norms, promises, and contradictions. (根据一个社会形式、理论或制度自身的规范、承诺和矛盾来评价它的批判。)  
**Problem solved:** it avoids external moralizing by showing how a form fails according to its own standards. (它通过显示一个形式按其自身标准而失败，避免外在道德说教。)  
**Why needed:** critique is stronger when it shows that a society betrays the very ideals it claims to uphold. (当批判显示一个社会背叛其自称维护的理想时，批判更有力量。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing contradictions between declared values and actual institutions. (当分析被宣称的价值与实际制度之间的矛盾时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Immanent critique is one of the most powerful tools inherited from Hegel and Marx. It does not simply impose an outside standard. It asks: what does this society claim to be? Does it realize its own promise?  
  
For example, a society may claim freedom while producing dependence; equality while preserving hierarchy; rationality while operating through manipulation; democracy while excluding voices.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Immanent critique shows that a form of life fails by the standards it gives itself. (内在批判显示一种生活形式按其自身给出的标准而失败。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **External Critique (外在批判; en: external critique)** judges from an outside norm; **Immanent Critique (内在批判; de: immanente Kritik)** judges by internal contradictions and unrealized promises. (外在批判从外部规范判断；内在批判通过内部矛盾和未实现承诺判断。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** immanent critique connects German Idealist contradiction with Marxian social critique and Critical Theory’s diagnosis of modern institutions. (内在批判把德国观念论的矛盾同马克思式社会批判和批判理论对现代制度的诊断连接起来。)  
  
### 21. Social Pathology: The Problem of Damaged Forms of Life  
  
`Social Pathology (社会病理; de: soziale Pathologie)`  
**Definition:** a systematic deformation of social life that damages autonomy, recognition, rationality, or flourishing. (对社会生活的系统性扭曲，它损害自主性、承认、理性或良好生活。)  
**Problem solved:** it gives critique a way to diagnose societies as unhealthy without reducing problems to individual defects. (它使批判能够诊断社会的不健康状态，而不把问题化约为个体缺陷。)  
**Why needed:** modern suffering often arises from normal institutions rather than exceptional breakdowns. (现代痛苦常来自正常制度，而不是例外性崩溃。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing alienation, reification, misrecognition, burnout, consumer dependency, social invisibility, or communicative distortion. (当分析异化、物化、误认、倦怠、消费依赖、社会不可见性或交往扭曲时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Social pathology treats society as capable of being distorted in its basic forms of life. The problem is not only that some people suffer. The problem is that social arrangements produce suffering while appearing normal.  
  
This concept connects Critical Theory with psychology, sociology, ethics, and political philosophy.  
  
**Typical sentence:** A social pathology is a normal social form that systematically damages the conditions of freedom or flourishing. (社会病理是一种正常化的社会形式，它系统性地损害自由或良好生活的条件。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Individual Pathology (个体病理; en: individual pathology)** locates disorder in persons; **Social Pathology (社会病理; de: soziale Pathologie)** locates disorder in social forms. (个体病理把失序定位于个人；社会病理把失序定位于社会形式。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** social pathology broadens critique from exploitation and ideology to damaged life-forms. (社会病理把批判从剥削和意识形态扩展到受损的生活形式。)  
  
### 22. Recognition Revisited: The Problem of Social Freedom  
  
`Recognition (承认; de: Anerkennung)`  
**Definition:** the social confirmation of persons or groups as bearers of dignity, rights, identity, and agency. (对个人或群体作为尊严、权利、身份和行动者性承担者的社会确认。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains how freedom depends on social relations rather than isolated choice alone. (它解释自由如何依赖社会关系，而不只是孤立选择。)  
**Why needed:** persons become socially real through recognition, and misrecognition can damage identity and agency. (人通过承认成为社会现实者，而误认会损害身份与行动者性。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing respect, rights, identity, social esteem, misrecognition, or struggles for justice. (当分析尊重、权利、身份、社会评价、误认或正义斗争时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Recognition appeared earlier in Hegel. Critical Theory renews it as a social diagnostic. Social domination is not only economic exploitation. It can also be misrecognition: being rendered invisible, inferior, deviant, dependent, or less than fully human.  
  
Recognition theory asks what forms of social relation are necessary for freedom: love, rights, solidarity, respect, and esteem.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Recognition is the social condition under which freedom becomes livable and identity becomes secure. (承认是自由变得可生活、身份变得稳定的社会条件。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Recognition (承认; de: Anerkennung)** differs from **Tolerance (宽容; en: tolerance)**. Tolerance may merely permit difference; recognition affirms status and standing. (宽容可能只是允许差异；承认则确认地位和资格。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** recognition connects Hegelian selfhood, existential otherness, feminist critique, postcolonial critique, and contemporary social justice theory. (承认连接黑格尔式自我性、存在主义他者问题、女性主义批判、后殖民批判和当代社会正义理论。)  
  
### 23. Hermeneutics versus Critical Theory: The Problem of Trust and Suspicion  
  
`Hermeneutics of Trust (信任的解释学; en: hermeneutics of trust)`  
**Definition:** an interpretive orientation that seeks to understand a text, tradition, or practice from within its own claim to meaning. (一种解释取向，它试图从文本、传统或实践自身的意义要求内部理解它。)  
**Problem solved:** it prevents premature reduction of meaning to hidden causes or interests. (它防止过早把意义化约为隐藏原因或利益。)  
**Why needed:** not every meaning is only a mask for domination. (并非每个意义都只是支配的面具。)  
**How to use:** use it when the first task is receptive understanding before critique. (当首要任务是在批判之前进行接受性理解时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
`Hermeneutics of Suspicion (怀疑的解释学; fr: herméneutique du soupçon)`  
**Definition:** an interpretive orientation that reads surface meanings as possibly concealing power, interest, repression, ideology, or domination. (一种解释取向，它把表层意义读作可能遮蔽权力、利益、压抑、意识形态或支配的东西。)  
**Problem solved:** it prevents naive acceptance of self-presented meaning. (它防止天真接受自我呈现的意义。)  
**Why needed:** social and psychic life often conceal their own conditions. (社会生活和心理生活常常遮蔽自身条件。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing ideology, repression, domination, ressentiment, or hidden function. (当分析意识形态、压抑、支配、怨恨或隐藏功能时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Hermeneutics and Critical Theory can conflict. Hermeneutics emphasizes belonging, tradition, and openness to meaning. Critical Theory worries that tradition may be domination, and openness may become obedience.  
  
The productive reading strategy is not to choose one permanently. It is to ask what the object requires.  
  
Some texts require patient internal understanding.  
(有些文本需要耐心的内部理解。)  
  
Some institutions require suspicion because their self-description is ideological.  
(有些制度需要怀疑，因为其自我描述是意识形态性的。)  
  
Some cases require both.  
(有些案例两者都需要。)  
  
**Typical sentence:** Trust asks what a text means; suspicion asks what that meaning hides or enables. (信任追问文本意味着什么；怀疑追问这种意义遮蔽或促成了什么。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Understanding (理解; de: Verstehen)** is not enough when meaning is distorted; **Critique (批判; de: Kritik)** is not enough when it refuses to understand what it criticizes. (当意义被扭曲时，理解并不足够；当批判拒绝理解其批判对象时，批判也不足够。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** modern interpretation becomes divided between receptivity and critique, belonging and emancipation, tradition and suspicion. (现代解释在接受性与批判、归属与解放、传统与怀疑之间分裂。)  
  
### 24. The Tool-Map of Hermeneutics and Critical Theory  
  
Use this chapter diagnostically. The central question is either **how meaning is historically understood** or **how understanding is socially distorted**.  
  
**If the text asks how meaning is understood across distance**, look for **Hermeneutics (解释学; de: Hermeneutik)**, **Interpretation (解释; de: Auslegung)**, and **Understanding (理解; de: Verstehen)**.  
(如果文本追问意义如何跨越距离而被理解，应寻找解释学、解释和理解问题。)  
  
**If the text moves between part and whole**, look for **Hermeneutic Circle (解释学循环; de: hermeneutischer Zirkel)**.  
(如果文本在部分与整体之间往返，应寻找解释学循环问题。)  
  
**If the text analyzes the interpreter’s historical situatedness**, look for **Prejudice (前见; de: Vorurteil)**, **Tradition (传统; de: Überlieferung)**, **Horizon (视域; de: Horizont)**, and **Effective History (效果历史; de: Wirkungsgeschichte)**.  
(如果文本分析解释者的历史处境性，应寻找前见、传统、视域和效果历史问题。)  
  
**If the text analyzes understanding between past and present**, look for **Fusion of Horizons (视域融合; de: Horizontverschmelzung)**.  
(如果文本分析过去与现在之间的理解，应寻找视域融合问题。)  
  
**If the text asks how reason becomes domination**, look for **Critical Theory (批判理论; de: Kritische Theorie)**, **Enlightenment (启蒙; de: Aufklärung)**, and **Instrumental Reason (工具理性; de: instrumentelle Vernunft)**.  
(如果文本追问理性如何成为支配，应寻找批判理论、启蒙和工具理性问题。)  
  
**If the text analyzes structural unfreedom**, look for **Domination (支配; de: Herrschaft)**, **Reification (物化; de: Verdinglichung)**, **Ideology (意识形态; de: Ideologie)**, and **Social Pathology (社会病理; de: soziale Pathologie)**.  
(如果文本分析结构性不自由，应寻找支配、物化、意识形态和社会病理问题。)  
  
**If the text analyzes culture and media as social control**, look for **Culture Industry (文化工业; de: Kulturindustrie)**.  
(如果文本把文化和媒体作为社会控制来分析，应寻找文化工业问题。)  
  
**If the text asks how critique can aim at freedom**, look for **Emancipation (解放; de: Emanzipation)**, **Communicative Rationality (交往理性; de: kommunikative Rationalität)**, and **Immanent Critique (内在批判; de: immanente Kritik)**.  
(如果文本追问批判如何以自由为目标，应寻找解放、交往理性和内在批判问题。)  
  
**If the text analyzes social identity and dignity**, look for **Recognition (承认; de: Anerkennung)** and **Misrecognition (误认; en: misrecognition)**.  
(如果文本分析社会身份与尊严，应寻找承认和误认问题。)  
  
### 25. The Genealogical Point of Part 11  
  
Hermeneutics and Critical Theory transform the problem of understanding. Analytic philosophy disciplines claims through argument and logic. Hermeneutics shows that meaning is historically mediated by language, tradition, prejudice, and horizon. Critical Theory shows that historical mediation may itself be distorted by domination, ideology, reification, and instrumental reason.  
  
The guiding thesis is:  
  
**Hermeneutic and critical-theoretical language turns understanding into a historically and socially mediated problem: to understand a meaning is to ask through what tradition, horizon, and interpretive relation it becomes intelligible; to criticize society is to ask how those very conditions of intelligibility are distorted by domination and how they might be transformed.**  
(解释学与批判理论语言把理解转化为历史和社会中介的问题：理解一个意义，就是追问它通过何种传统、视域和解释关系成为可理解之物；批判社会，则是追问这些可理解性的条件如何被支配扭曲，以及它们如何可能被转化。)  
  
This grammar prepares the next stages. Structuralism will shift attention from historical understanding to underlying systems of signs and relations. Post-structuralism will question whether meaning, subject, and structure can ever be stabilized. Derrida will radicalize interpretation by showing how texts depend on difference, trace, and supplement. Foucault will transform critique by analyzing how discourses, institutions, and power relations produce subjects and truths.  
  
The hermeneutic-critical question remains a durable tool for philosophical reading:  
  
**What horizon makes this meaning intelligible, and what forms of power may be shaping that horizon?**  
(什么视域使这个意义成为可理解之物？又有哪些权力形式可能正在塑造这个视域？)  
  
## Part 12. Structuralism and Post-Structuralism: Sign, Difference, Decentering  
  
This chapter explains how structuralism and post-structuralism transform the problem of meaning. Hermeneutics had asked how meaning is historically understood through tradition, horizon, and interpretation. Critical Theory had asked how understanding is distorted by ideology, domination, and instrumental reason. Structuralism changes the question: **what underlying system makes meaning possible before any individual speaker, author, or subject intends it?** (在任何个体说话者、作者或主体意图之前，是什么底层系统使意义成为可能？)  
  
Post-structuralism then radicalizes the problem: **if meaning depends on differential systems, can meaning ever become fully stable, present, or final?** (如果意义依赖差异系统，那么意义是否能够完全稳定、完全在场或最终确定？)  
  
The central vocabulary is **Sign**, **Signifier**, **Signified**, **Structure**, **System**, **Difference**, **Langue**, **Parole**, **Code**, **Binary Opposition**, **Myth**, **Text**, **Intertextuality**, **Decentering**, **Différance**, **Trace**, **Supplement**, **Deconstruction**, **Logocentrism**, **Discourse**, and **Subject-Position**. Saussurean sign theory analyzes the sign through **signifier** and **signified**; structuralism treats meaning as produced by systems of difference; post-structuralism stresses instability, deferral, and Derrida’s **différance**.  
  
The operational function of this chapter is precise: use structuralist vocabulary when the problem is **how meaning is produced by a system of relations**; use post-structuralist vocabulary when the problem is **how that system fails to close, stabilizes through exclusions, or produces effects of presence and authority**. (当问题是意义如何由关系系统生产时，应使用结构主义词汇；当问题是这一系统如何无法封闭、如何通过排除而稳定、如何生产在场与权威效果时，应使用后结构主义词汇。)  
  
### 1. The Problem-Situation: From Meaning as Intention to Meaning as System  
  
Before structuralism, meaning is often explained through **authorial intention**, **consciousness**, **reference**, **historical tradition**, or **lived experience**. A speaker means something. A subject intends an object. A tradition transmits meaning. A text expresses an author’s thought. These models are not useless, but structuralism asks whether they begin too late.  
  
The structuralist question is:  
  
**What system must already exist for an individual expression to mean anything?**  
(为了使一个个体表达能够具有意义，必须已经存在什么系统？)  
  
A word does not mean by itself. A kinship role does not mean by itself. A legal category does not mean by itself. A gender identity, literary trope, mythic opposition, currency symbol, national flag, academic credential, or algorithmic label does not mean by itself. Each functions within a system of differences, rules, positions, and oppositions.  
  
This is why structuralism is anti-individualist at the level of meaning. It does not begin from the self-transparent subject. It begins from systems.  
  
Post-structuralism then asks:  
  
**If meaning depends on systems of difference, why assume the system is stable, centered, or closed?**  
(如果意义依赖差异系统，为什么要假设这一系统是稳定的、有中心的或封闭的？)  
  
This is the transition from structure to instability, from system to play, from sign to trace, from centered meaning to deferred meaning.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Structuralism asks what system makes meaning possible; post-structuralism asks why that system cannot finally stabilize meaning. (结构主义追问什么系统使意义成为可能；后结构主义追问为什么该系统无法最终稳定意义。)  
  
### 2. Sign: The Problem of Meaning as Mediation  
  
`Sign (符号; la: signum; fr: signe)`  
**Definition:** a unit that signifies by standing within a system of differences and conventions. (一种通过处于差异与约定系统中而进行表意的单位。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains meaning as mediated rather than naturally transparent. (它把意义解释为被中介的，而非自然透明的。)  
**Why needed:** human meaning does not arise from isolated objects or sounds; it arises from signifying systems. (人类意义并不从孤立对象或声音中自然生长，而是从表意系统中产生。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing words, images, gestures, legal marks, money, uniforms, rituals, myths, brands, or data labels as meaning-bearing units. (当分析词语、图像、手势、法律标记、货币、制服、仪式、神话、品牌或数据标签作为承载意义的单位时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
A sign is not merely a label attached to a thing. A sign works because a system allows it to work. A red traffic light means stop only within a traffic code. A passport means citizenship or mobility only within state systems. A diploma means qualification only within educational and labor-market institutions. A username, verification badge, risk score, or recommendation category means something only within digital systems of classification.  
  
Examples such as flags, uniforms, passports, money, police badges, academic credentials, brands, algorithmic labels, and data profiles make the point concrete: these are not ordinary physical objects once placed inside sign systems; they organize loyalty, identity, authority, value, access, and institutional response.  
  
**Typical sentence:** A sign does not carry meaning naturally; it functions within a system that makes it readable. (符号并不天然携带意义；它在一个使其可读的系统中运作。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Sign (符号; fr: signe)** differs from **Thing (事物; la: res)**. A thing may exist physically; a sign functions by signifying within a system. (事物可以物理地存在；符号则通过在系统中表意而发挥功能。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** sign theory transforms philosophy of language, anthropology, literary theory, law, media studies, and social critique. Meaning becomes a problem of systems, not merely names, intentions, or references. (符号理论改造语言哲学、人类学、文学理论、法学、媒介研究和社会批判。意义成为系统问题，而不只是名称、意图或指称问题。)  
  
### 3. Signifier and Signified: The Problem of the Sign’s Internal Structure  
  
`Signifier (能指; fr: signifiant)`  
**Definition:** in strict Saussurean linguistics, the acoustic image associated with a sign; in broader semiotic use, the perceptible sign-form such as sound, mark, image, gesture, or symbol-form. (在严格的索绪尔语言学中，能指是与符号相联系的声音形象；在广义符号学中，它可扩展为声音、标记、图像、手势或符号形式等可感知的符号形式。)  
**Problem solved:** it distinguishes the sign-form from the concept signified. (它把符号形式同被表意的概念区分开来。)  
**Why needed:** meaning cannot be analyzed if sign-form and sign-content are collapsed. (如果符号形式与符号内容被混同，意义就无法被分析。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing the form through which meaning is carried, produced, or differentially organized. (当分析意义借以被承载、生产或差异化组织的形式时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
**Usage layers:**  
1. **Strict Saussurean use (严格索绪尔用法):** the **signifier** is the acoustic image associated with a sign, not the external object and not simply the physical sound. (能指是与符号相关联的声音形象，不是外部对象，也不只是物理声音。)  
  
2. **Structuralist / semiotic reception use (结构主义/符号学接受史用法):** the signifier may be generalized to mark, image, sound pattern, written form, or symbolic form within a system of differences. (在结构主义和符号学接受史中，能指可扩展为差异系统中的标记、图像、声音模式、书写形式或符号形式。)  
  
3. **Lacanian / poststructuralist use (拉康式/后结构主义用法):** the signifier is not merely a sign-form; it can structure subjectivity, desire, unconscious formation, symbolic position, and social recognition. (在拉康和后结构主义语境中，能指不只是符号形式，还可结构主体性、欲望、无意识形成、象征位置和社会承认。)  
  
**Transfer rule:** before using **signifier**, decide whether the analysis concerns linguistic sign-structure, semiotic form, symbolic order, unconscious desire, or social recognition. (转用规则：使用 signifier 之前，应先判断分析对象是语言符号结构、符号形式、象征秩序、无意识欲望，还是社会承认。)  
  
**Misuse warning:** **Signifier** is not the same as word, label, symbol, or referent. (Signifier 不等于词、标签、符号或指称对象。)  
  
`Signified (所指; fr: signifié)`  
**Definition:** the concept associated with a signifier within a language system, not the external object itself. (在语言系统内部同能指相联系的概念，而不是外部对象本身。)  
**Problem solved:** it distinguishes conceptual content from sound, mark, and external referent. (它把概念内容同声音、标记和外部指称对象区分开来。)  
**Why needed:** comparable objects may be associated with different signifieds across languages, because each language organizes conceptual differences in its own system. (不同语言可以指向相近对象，但其所指并不保证完全相同，因为每种语言都在自身系统中组织概念差异。)
