**How to use:** use it when analyzing what concept a signifier evokes within a system. (当分析一个能指在系统中唤起什么概念时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
**Usage layers:**  
1. **Strict Saussurean use (严格索绪尔用法):** the **signified** is the concept associated with a signifier inside a language system, not the external object itself. (所指是在语言系统内部同能指相联系的概念，而不是外部对象本身。)  
  
2. **Structuralist reception use (结构主义接受史用法):** the signified is understood differentially: it is shaped by its place in a system of contrasts, not by an isolated one-to-one link with a thing. (在结构主义接受史中，所指以差异方式被理解：它由系统中的对立位置塑造，而不是由同某物的一对一孤立关系塑造。)  
  
3. **Poststructuralist transferable use (后结构主义泛用法):** in poststructuralist contexts, the stability of the signified is questioned; meaning is treated as deferred, relational, and exposed to slippage. (在后结构主义语境中，所指的稳定性受到质疑；意义被视为延异的、关系性的，并且容易发生滑移。)  
  
**Transfer rule:** do not treat the signified as the physical object referred to. Ask whether the analysis concerns concept, referent, meaning-effect, or unstable semantic position. (转用规则：不要把所指当成被指称的物理对象。应判断分析对象是概念、指称对象、意义效果，还是不稳定的语义位置。)  
  
**Misuse warning:** **Signified** is not identical with referent. (Signified 不等同于 referent。)  
  
Saussure’s basic insight is that the linguistic sign consists of signifier and signified. The English sound-image *tree*, the written mark “tree,” French *arbre*, Chinese “树,” and Japanese “木” can be treated as comparable signifiers in a broad semiotic comparison, but in strict Saussurean terms each belongs to a different language system and does not simply express an identical signified.  
  
This distinction prevents a naive theory of meaning. Words are not natural extensions of things. Sounds do not contain meaning by themselves. Meaning emerges because a language system links signifiers and signifieds in regulated ways.  
  
**Typical sentence:** The signifier is the form that signifies; the signified is the concept signified. (能指是进行表意的形式；所指是被表意的概念。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Referent (指称对象; en: referent)** is the object or entity referred to; **Signified (所指; fr: signifié)** is the concept within the sign. (指称对象是被指向的对象或实体；所指是符号内部的概念内容。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** this distinction changes the philosophy of language from word-object correspondence toward sign-system analysis. (这一区分把语言哲学从词—物符合关系转向符号系统分析。)  
  
### 4. Arbitrariness: The Problem of Non-Natural Meaning  
  
`Arbitrariness of the Sign (符号任意性; fr: arbitraire du signe)`  
**Definition:** the principle that the relation between signifier and signified is not naturally necessary but conventionally established. (能指与所指之间的关系并非自然必然，而是由约定建立的原则。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains why different languages can use different forms for similar concepts. (它解释为什么不同语言可以用不同形式表达相近概念。)  
**Why needed:** without arbitrariness, meaning would be mistaken for a natural property of sounds or marks. (如果没有任意性原则，意义就会被误认为声音或标记的自然属性。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing why a sign’s meaning depends on convention and system rather than natural resemblance. (当分析为什么符号意义依赖约定和系统，而非自然相似性时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Arbitrariness does not mean randomness. Once a language community stabilizes a sign, individuals cannot simply change it at will and expect to be understood. The sign is arbitrary in origin or relation, but structured in use.  
  
This distinction matters. If arbitrariness is misunderstood as “anything can mean anything,” structuralism collapses into caricature. Structuralism does not say signs are free-floating nonsense. It says signs are governed by systems rather than nature.  
  
**Typical sentence:** The sign is arbitrary in relation, but not arbitrary in social use. (符号在关系上是任意的，但在社会使用中并非任意。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Arbitrary (任意的; fr: arbitraire)** in structural linguistics means non-natural relation; **Random (随机的; en: random)** means lacking pattern or rule. (结构语言学中的任意意味着非自然关系；随机意味着缺乏模式或规则。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** arbitrariness allows later theory to analyze social classifications as constructed without calling them unreal. Gender categories, legal identities, money, nationality, and institutional roles are not natural in a simple sense, but they can be socially real. (任意性使后来的理论能够分析社会分类的建构性，而不必说它们不真实。性别分类、法律身份、货币、国籍和制度角色并非简单自然之物，但它们可以具有社会现实性。)  
  
### 5. Difference: The Problem of Relational Meaning  
  
`Difference (差异; la: differentia; fr: différence)`  
**Definition:** the relational distinction through which signs and concepts receive value within a system. (符号和概念在系统中获得价值的关系性区别。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains why meaning comes from position and contrast rather than isolated substance. (它解释为什么意义来自位置与对照，而非孤立实体。)  
**Why needed:** a sign means by not being other signs. (一个符号通过不是其他符号而具有意义。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing conceptual oppositions, classificatory systems, semantic fields, or social categories. (当分析概念对立、分类系统、语义场或社会类别时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Difference is the structuralist engine. “Legal” means what it means through contrast with “illegal.” “Nature” means through contrast with “culture.” “Male” and “female,” “civilized” and “barbaric,” “normal” and “deviant,” “citizen” and “foreigner,” “expert” and “layperson” are not merely pairs of words. They organize social reality.  
  
Meaning is not only produced by reference to objects, but by difference within a language system; oppositions such as male/female, nature/culture, civilized/barbaric, rational/sensible, legal/illegal organize entire spaces of meaning.  
  
**Typical sentence:** A term has meaning not by standing alone, but by occupying a position in a system of differences. (一个术语不是通过孤立存在而有意义，而是通过在差异系统中占据位置而有意义。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Positive Meaning (正面意义; en: positive meaning)** treats a term as self-contained; **Differential Meaning (差异性意义; fr: sens différentiel)** treats meaning as produced through contrast. (正面意义把术语视为自足；差异性意义把意义视为通过对照而生产。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** difference prepares post-structuralism. If meaning is differential, then no sign can fully possess meaning in itself. Meaning always points elsewhere. (差异为后结构主义做准备。如果意义是差异性的，那么没有符号能够完全在自身中拥有意义。意义总是指向别处。)  
  
### 6. Structure: The Problem of Relations over Elements  
  
`Structure (结构; la: structura; fr: structure)`  
**Definition:** an organized system of relations in which elements receive function and meaning from their positions. (一种有组织的关系系统，其中元素从其位置获得功能和意义。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains why elements cannot be understood in isolation. (它解释为什么元素不能被孤立理解。)  
**Why needed:** linguistic, social, mythical, literary, kinship, legal, and cultural systems work by relations. (语言、社会、神话、文学、亲属、法律和文化系统通过关系运作。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing the underlying relational order that makes surface phenomena intelligible. (当分析使表层现象成为可理解之物的底层关系秩序时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
**Transfer rule:** use **Structure** when relations organize the function, meaning, or position of elements; do not use it merely to mean arrangement, outline, or visible organization. (转用规则：当关系组织了元素的功能、意义或位置时，才使用 Structure；不要把它仅仅当成排列、提纲或可见组织。)  
  
A structure is not just a collection. A chess piece means what it means only within chess rules. A legal role means what it means only within legal institutions. A kinship term means what it means only within a kinship system. A mythic figure means what it means only within a network of oppositions and transformations.  
  
Structuralist analysis therefore asks:  
  
**What position does this element occupy in the system?**  
(这个元素在系统中占据什么位置？)  
  
**What oppositions organize the system?**  
(什么对立组织了这一系统？)  
  
**What transformations preserve the structure while changing the surface form?**  
(什么转化在改变表层形式的同时保持了结构？)  
  
**Typical sentence:** A structure is the relational order through which elements become meaningful. (结构是元素借以成为有意义者的关系秩序。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Aggregate (集合; de: Aggregat)** is a mere collection of elements; **Structure (结构; fr: structure)** is a relational system in which elements have positions and functions. (集合是元素的单纯聚集；结构则是元素具有位置和功能的关系系统。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** structure displaces the subject. Meaning is no longer grounded primarily in individual consciousness, but in systems that precede and exceed the individual. (结构移置主体。意义不再首先奠基于个体意识，而是奠基于先于并超出个体的系统。)  
  
### 7. System: The Problem of Rule-Governed Meaning  
  
`System (系统; el: σύστημα; fr: système)`  
**Definition:** a rule-governed whole in which units function by relation, difference, and position. (一个受规则支配的整体，其中单位通过关系、差异和位置运作。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains stability in meaning without appealing to natural essence. (它在不诉诸自然本质的情况下解释意义稳定性。)  
**Why needed:** signs are arbitrary in relation, but systemically constrained in use. (符号在关系上任意，但在使用中受系统约束。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing the grammar, code, institution, classification, or symbolic order that regulates meaning. (当分析规制意义的语法、代码、制度、分类或符号秩序时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
**Transfer rule:** use **System** when elements gain meaning or function from an internally organized whole; do not use it for any mere collection, list, network, or large object. (转用规则：当元素从内部组织起来的整体中获得意义或功能时，才使用 System；不要把它用于任何单纯集合、列表、网络或大型对象。)  
  
The system is what prevents signs from becoming random. Language, law, kinship, ritual, fashion, academic ranking, digital identity, and money all require systems. A banknote is not valuable because of its paper substance. It is valuable because it is positioned within monetary, legal, institutional, and trust systems.  
  
The same applies to social categories. A title such as “judge,” “citizen,” “employee,” “patient,” “minor,” “refugee,” or “verified user” has force because it belongs to a system of recognition and consequences.  
  
**Typical sentence:** A system stabilizes meaning by regulating the relations among signs. (系统通过规制符号之间的关系来稳定意义。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **System (系统; fr: système)** differs from **Context (语境; la: contextus)**. Context is the surrounding situation; system is the organized structure of relations that makes signs function. (语境是周围情境；系统是使符号运作的有组织关系结构。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** system-thinking allows philosophy to analyze meaning, society, law, media, and digital classification without reducing them to individual intentions. (系统思维使哲学能够分析意义、社会、法律、媒介和数字分类，而不把它们化约为个体意图。)  
  
### 8. Langue and Parole: The Problem of System and Use  
  
`Langue (语言系统; fr: langue)`  
**Definition:** the structured system of language shared by a community. (一个共同体共享的结构化语言系统。)  
**Problem solved:** it distinguishes the underlying system from individual speech acts. (它把底层系统同个体言语行为区分开来。)  
**Why needed:** individual utterances are possible only because a language system already exists. (个体话语之所以可能，是因为语言系统已经存在。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing grammar, code, rules, and shared linguistic structure. (当分析语法、代码、规则和共享语言结构时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
`Parole (言语活动; fr: parole)`  
**Definition:** individual acts of speech or language use. (个体的说话行为或语言使用。)  
**Problem solved:** it distinguishes concrete utterance from the underlying system that makes utterance meaningful. (它把具体话语同使话语有意义的底层系统区分开来。)  
**Why needed:** one must not confuse individual expression with the structure that enables expression. (不能把个体表达同使表达成为可能的结构混淆。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing particular speech acts, texts, utterances, or performances. (当分析具体言语行为、文本、话语或表演时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
The distinction between *langue* and *parole* is a model for structuralist thinking generally. Individual acts presuppose systems. A sentence presupposes grammar. A legal decision presupposes a legal code. A ritual act presupposes ritual structure. A social performance presupposes social codes.  
  
This does not make individuals irrelevant. It means individual expression becomes analyzable only in relation to a prior system.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Parole is the individual use; langue is the system that makes use intelligible. (Parole 是个体使用；langue 是使使用成为可理解的系统。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Langue (语言系统; fr: langue)** differs from **Language in general (语言; en: language)**. Langue names a structured social system; language in general can name the broader human capacity or phenomenon. (Langue 命名结构化社会系统；一般意义上的语言可以指更宽的人类能力或现象。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** the langue/parole distinction becomes a template for analyzing culture: myth-system/event, legal code/case, social structure/action, symbolic order/performance. (Langue/parole 区分成为分析文化的模板：神话系统/事件、法律代码/案件、社会结构/行动、符号秩序/表演。)  
  
### 9. Synchrony and Diachrony: The Problem of System and History  
  
`Synchrony (共时性; fr: synchronie)`  
**Definition:** analysis of a system at a given moment as a structured whole. (在某一时刻把系统作为结构化整体来分析。)  
**Problem solved:** it reveals how meaning depends on relations within a current system. (它揭示意义如何依赖当前系统内部关系。)  
**Why needed:** one cannot understand a system only by tracing its historical origin. (不能只通过追溯历史起源来理解一个系统。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing the current relational organization of signs, rules, or categories. (当分析符号、规则或类别当前的关系组织时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
`Diachrony (历时性; fr: diachronie)`  
**Definition:** analysis of change across time. (对跨时间变化的分析。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains transformation, development, and historical sequence. (它解释转化、发展和历史序列。)  
**Why needed:** systems change, and meaning shifts across time. (系统会变化，意义会随时间转移。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing historical evolution of signs, concepts, institutions, or practices. (当分析符号、概念、制度或实践的历史演变时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Structuralism often privileges synchronic analysis. It asks how the system functions now, not only how it historically arose. This is useful because origin does not automatically explain current function.  
  
For example, the historical origin of a legal term may differ from its current function in a legal system. The etymology of a word may not explain its current meaning. A ritual may have one origin but another contemporary structure.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Synchrony analyzes the system as structured now; diachrony analyzes its transformation through time. (共时性分析系统现在如何被结构化；历时性分析系统如何随时间转化。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Genealogy (谱系学; de: Genealogie; fr: généalogie)** is not simply diachrony. Genealogy traces contingent formation, struggle, power, and descent; diachrony more broadly tracks temporal change. (谱系学不只是历时性。谱系学追踪偶然形成、斗争、权力和来源；历时性更广泛地追踪时间变化。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** structuralism temporarily brackets history to analyze system; post-structuralism and Foucault later bring history back as discontinuity, archive, discourse, and power. (结构主义暂时括号化历史以分析系统；后结构主义与福柯后来以断裂、档案、话语和权力的方式把历史带回。)  
  
### 10. Code: The Problem of Cultural Readability  
  
`Code (代码/符码; fr: code)`  
**Definition:** a rule-system that makes signs readable and actions intelligible. (使符号可读、行动可理解的规则系统。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains why cultural meanings can be learned, repeated, recognized, and misread. (它解释文化意义为何能够被学习、重复、识别和误读。)  
**Why needed:** signs require conventions for interpretation. (符号需要解释约定。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing cultural conventions, narrative rules, fashion, ritual, legal categories, media genres, or digital classifications. (当分析文化约定、叙事规则、时尚、仪式、法律类别、媒介类型或数字分类时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
A code is what makes a gesture polite or insulting, a garment formal or casual, a visual style official or rebellious, a legal mark valid or invalid, a data label actionable or meaningless. Codes do not merely reflect reality; they organize perception and response.  
  
A courtroom has codes. A university has codes. A hospital has codes. A social media platform has codes. A dating app, border control system, credit system, or academic peer-review system also has codes. These codes classify, authorize, exclude, rank, and normalize.  
  
**Typical sentence:** A code is the rule-system that lets signs and actions be read within a culture or institution. (符码是使符号和行动能够在文化或制度中被读取的规则系统。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Code (符码; fr: code)** differs from **Message (信息; fr: message)**. A message is what is communicated; a code is the system that makes communication readable. (信息是被传达之物；符码是使传达可读的系统。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** code becomes a bridge to media theory, semiotics, cybernetics, law, digital governance, and platform analysis. (符码成为通向媒介理论、符号学、控制论、法学、数字治理和平台分析的桥梁。)  
  
### 11. Binary Opposition: The Problem of Meaning through Hierarchy  
  
`Binary Opposition (二元对立; fr: opposition binaire)`  
**Definition:** a pair of opposed terms that structures meaning by contrast, often hierarchically. (通过对照来结构化意义的一组对立项，常具有等级性。)  
**Problem solved:** it identifies the oppositional structures that organize concepts, myths, institutions, and identities. (它识别组织概念、神话、制度和身份的对立结构。)  
**Why needed:** cultures often produce meaning by arranging terms into opposed pairs. (文化常通过把术语排列为对立项来生产意义。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing nature/culture, male/female, speech/writing, mind/body, civilized/barbaric, normal/deviant, legal/illegal, human/animal. (当分析自然/文化、男/女、言语/书写、心灵/身体、文明/野蛮、正常/异常、合法/非法、人/动物时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Binary opposition is central to both structuralism and post-structuralism. Structuralism uses binaries to analyze systems. Post-structuralism asks how binaries are unstable and hierarchical.  
  
For example, speech/writing is not a neutral pair in much of Western philosophy. Speech is often privileged as closer to presence, intention, voice, and meaning; writing is treated as secondary, derivative, or dangerous. Derrida’s critique begins from such hierarchies.  
  
**Typical sentence:** A binary opposition does not merely distinguish terms; it often ranks them and organizes a field of meaning around that rank. (二元对立并不只是区分术语；它常常对术语排序，并围绕这种排序组织意义场。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Distinction (区分; la: distinctio)** can be neutral; **Binary Opposition (二元对立; fr: opposition binaire)** often organizes hierarchy and exclusion. (区分可以是中性的；二元对立常组织等级和排除。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** binary analysis becomes a major tool for feminism, postcolonial theory, critical race theory, queer theory, legal critique, and deconstruction. (二元对立分析成为女性主义、后殖民理论、批判种族理论、酷儿理论、法律批判和解构的重要工具。)  
  
### 12. Myth: The Problem of Cultural Structure  
  
`Myth (神话; el: μῦθος; fr: mythe)`  
**Definition:** a narrative or symbolic system that organizes cultural meaning through recurring oppositions, transformations, and codes. (一种通过反复出现的对立、转化和符码来组织文化意义的叙事或符号系统。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains cultural narratives as structured systems rather than mere stories. (它把文化叙事解释为结构化系统，而不只是故事。)  
**Why needed:** societies encode contradictions and classifications through narrative forms. (社会通过叙事形式编码矛盾和分类。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing myths, rituals, national narratives, advertisements, origin stories, family scripts, or ideological plots. (当分析神话、仪式、民族叙事、广告、起源故事、家庭脚本或意识形态情节时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
For structural anthropology, myth is not primitive error. It is a symbolic mechanism. Myths organize contradictions: nature/culture, raw/cooked, life/death, human/animal, kin/stranger, purity/pollution. They do not merely say something. They structure what can be thought.  
  
Modern societies also produce myths. The “self-made individual,” “free market,” “neutral technology,” “model minority,” “civilizing mission,” “meritocracy,” and “national destiny” can function mythically. They organize contradictions and make social arrangements appear meaningful.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Myth is not merely false story; it is a symbolic structure that organizes cultural contradictions. (神话不只是虚假故事，而是组织文化矛盾的符号结构。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Myth (神话; fr: mythe)** differs from **Lie (谎言; en: lie)**. A lie intentionally deceives; myth structures collective meaning, whether or not anyone deliberately fabricates it. (谎言有意欺骗；神话结构集体意义，不必有某个人蓄意编造。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** myth-analysis links structuralism with ideology critique. It shows how cultural narratives can naturalize social order. (神话分析把结构主义同意识形态批判连接起来，显示文化叙事如何自然化社会秩序。)  
  
### 13. Decentering: The Problem of the Subject after Structure  
  
`Decentering (去中心化; fr: décentrement)`  
**Definition:** the displacement of the human subject from the position of origin, master, or center of meaning. (把人类主体从意义的起源、主人或中心位置上移开的过程。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains why meaning, desire, language, and identity are not fully controlled by conscious intention. (它解释为什么意义、欲望、语言和身份并不完全由意识意图控制。)  
**Why needed:** the subject speaks through systems it did not create and is shaped by structures it does not fully know. (主体通过并非由其创造的系统说话，并被其无法完全知道的结构塑造。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing language, unconscious, ideology, discourse, social codes, or subject-positions as prior to individual self-mastery. (当分析语言、无意识、意识形态、话语、社会符码或主体位置如何先于个体自我主宰时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Structuralism decentrers the subject by showing that language speaks through the speaker. Psychoanalysis decentrers the subject by showing that desire exceeds conscious control. Marxism decentrers the subject by showing that social relations shape consciousness. Post-structuralism intensifies this: the subject is not origin but effect.  
  
This does not mean persons do not exist. It means that “the subject” is not the sovereign foundation of meaning.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Decentering means that the subject is no longer the origin of meaning, but a position within systems of language, desire, power, and discourse. (去中心化意味着主体不再是意义的起源，而是语言、欲望、权力和话语系统中的一个位置。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Subject (主体; la: subiectum; fr: sujet)** in modern philosophy is often treated as ground; **Subject-Position (主体位置; fr: position de sujet)** treats subjectivity as produced within systems. (现代哲学中的主体常被视为根据；主体位置则把主体性视为在系统中被生产出来。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** decentering prepares Foucault, Derrida, Lacan, Althusser, feminist theory, and postcolonial theory. It makes subjectivity an object of analysis rather than the unquestioned starting point. (去中心化为福柯、德里达、拉康、阿尔都塞、女性主义理论和后殖民理论做准备。它使主体性成为分析对象，而非未经质疑的出发点。)  
  
### 14. Text: The Problem of Meaning beyond Authorial Intention  
  
`Text (文本; la: textus; fr: texte)`  
**Definition:** a woven field of signs, codes, differences, references, and interpretive possibilities. (由符号、符码、差异、指涉和解释可能性编织成的场域。)  
**Problem solved:** it shifts reading from authorial intention alone to textual structure and signifying play. (它把阅读从单纯作者意图转向文本结构和表意运动。)  
**Why needed:** meaning can exceed what an author consciously intends. (意义可以超出作者有意识的意图。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing literature, law, philosophy, media, institutions, bodies, cities, or digital systems as signifying fields. (当把文学、法律、哲学、媒体、制度、身体、城市或数字系统作为表意场域来分析时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
A text is not merely a written document. In structuralist and post-structuralist theory, a text is any organized field of signs. A legal code is a text. A building can be read as a text. A fashion system, social media profile, courtroom ritual, national ceremony, or medical form can be analyzed textually.  
  
This does not mean everything is “just text” in a trivial sense. It means that social reality is mediated by signifying systems.  
  
**Typical sentence:** A text is not a container of authorial intention, but a field where signs produce meaning through relations and differences. (文本不是作者意图的容器，而是符号通过关系和差异生产意义的场域。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Work (作品; fr: œuvre)** can suggest a bounded object attributed to an author; **Text (文本; fr: texte)** emphasizes signifying relations, plurality, and readability. (作品暗示归属于作者的有边界对象；文本强调表意关系、复数性和可读性。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** text theory transforms literary analysis and spreads into law, anthropology, cultural studies, media theory, and social theory. (文本理论改造文学分析，并扩展到法学、人类学、文化研究、媒介理论和社会理论。)  
  
### 15. Intertextuality: The Problem of No Isolated Text  
  
`Intertextuality (互文性; fr: intertextualité)`  
**Definition:** the relation by which any text is shaped by other texts, codes, genres, quotations, echoes, and prior meanings. (任何文本都由其他文本、符码、文类、引文、回声和先前意义塑造的关系。)  
**Problem solved:** it prevents the text from being treated as self-contained. (它防止文本被视为自足对象。)  
**Why needed:** meanings circulate across texts before and beyond any single author. (意义在任何单一作者之前并超出其范围，在文本之间流通。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing citation, genre, adaptation, parody, legal precedent, philosophical inheritance, cultural memory, or media remix. (当分析引用、文类、改编、戏仿、法律先例、哲学继承、文化记忆或媒介混剪时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
No text begins from nothing. A philosophical essay echoes prior arguments. A court judgment cites precedent. A novel rewrites genres. A political slogan condenses older myths. A meme depends on shared templates. A social media post is legible because it belongs to recognizable formats.  
  
Intertextuality therefore weakens the fantasy of pure origin. Meaning is inherited, repeated, altered, and displaced.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Intertextuality means that every text is crossed by other texts before it speaks in its own name. (互文性意味着每个文本在以自身名义说话之前已经被其他文本穿过。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Influence (影响; en: influence)** suggests one source affecting another; **Intertextuality (互文性; fr: intertextualité)** suggests a broader field of textual relations without a single origin. (影响暗示一个来源作用于另一个文本；互文性则暗示没有单一起源的更广文本关系场。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** intertextuality turns tradition into textual circulation and prepares deconstruction’s critique of origin, presence, and self-contained meaning. (互文性把传统转化为文本流通，并为解构对起源、在场和自足意义的批判做准备。)  
  
### 16. Post-Structuralism: The Problem of Unstable Systems  
  
`Post-Structuralism (后结构主义; fr: post-structuralisme)`  
**Definition:** a set of approaches that inherit structuralism’s focus on systems and difference while questioning stability, closure, center, and fixed meaning. (一组继承结构主义对系统和差异的关注，同时质疑稳定性、封闭性、中心和固定意义的方法。)  
**Problem solved:** it exposes the instability inside signifying systems and conceptual hierarchies. (它揭示表意系统与概念等级内部的不稳定性。)  
**Why needed:** if meaning depends on relations, then meaning cannot finally rest in a self-present origin. (如果意义依赖关系，那么意义就不能最终安放在自我在场的起源中。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing slippage, undecidability, exclusion, textual instability, discourse, power, and the decentered subject. (当分析滑动、不可判定性、排除、文本不稳定性、话语、权力和去中心化主体时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Post-structuralism is often misread as saying “nothing means anything.” That is inaccurate. It says meaning is produced, stabilized, contested, deferred, and destabilized through systems that never fully close.  
  
Post-structuralism should not be treated as mere relativism: it stresses that meaning slides, delays, and splits, but this does not mean language has no meaning; it means meaning never appears as complete self-sufficient presence.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Post-structuralism does not abolish meaning; it analyzes why meaning is produced without becoming finally closed. (后结构主义并不取消意义；它分析意义为何被生产却无法最终封闭。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Structuralism (结构主义; fr: structuralisme)** emphasizes system and relation; **Post-Structuralism (后结构主义; fr: post-structuralisme)** emphasizes instability, displacement, and the failure of closure within systems. (结构主义强调系统与关系；后结构主义强调系统内部的不稳定、位移和封闭失败。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** post-structuralism turns structuralism against itself. The same difference that makes meaning possible also prevents meaning from becoming final. (后结构主义使结构主义反转自身。使意义成为可能的差异，也使意义无法成为最终意义。)  
  
### 17. Différance: The Problem of Difference and Deferral  
  
`Différance (延异; fr: différance)`  
**Definition:** Derrida’s term for the production of meaning through both difference and deferral. (德里达用来指意义通过差异与延迟共同被生产的术语。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains why meaning is never fully present at one point. (它解释为什么意义从不在某一点上完全在场。)  
**Why needed:** signs mean by differing from other signs and by referring onward to further signs. (符号通过不同于其他符号而表意，并通过继续指向更多符号而表意。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing how meaning depends on differential spacing and temporal delay. (当分析意义如何依赖差异性间隔与时间性延迟时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
**Différance** is deliberately not the ordinary French *différence*. It combines *to differ* and *to defer*. Meaning arises because a sign differs from other signs, but the sign never delivers final meaning immediately. It sends interpretation onward.  
  
The word itself performs the point. In French pronunciation, *différence* and *différance* sound the same. The difference appears in writing, not speech. This challenges the traditional privilege of speech over writing.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Différance means that meaning is generated by difference and postponed through further reference. (延异意味着意义由差异生成，并通过进一步指涉而被推迟。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Difference (差异; fr: différence)** marks distinction; **Différance (延异; fr: différance)** marks distinction plus deferral and spacing. (差异标记区别；延异标记区别加延迟和间隔化。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** différance radicalizes Saussurean difference and Heideggerian absence/presence problems. It becomes a tool for criticizing metaphysics of full presence. (延异激进化索绪尔式差异和海德格尔式在场/缺席问题，成为批判完整在场形而上学的工具。)  
  
### 18. Trace: The Problem of Absence within Presence  
  
`Trace (痕迹; fr: trace)`  
**Definition:** the mark of other signs, absences, and prior differences within any present meaning. (任何当前意义内部的其他符号、缺席和先前差异的标记。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains why no sign is purely self-present. (它解释为什么没有符号能够纯粹自我在场。)  
**Why needed:** a sign carries what it is not as part of how it means. (一个符号把其所不是之物作为其表意方式的一部分携带着。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing how excluded, absent, past, or deferred elements remain active inside meaning. (当分析被排除的、缺席的、过去的或被延迟的元素如何仍在意义内部发挥作用时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
A trace is not a visible mark only. It is the structural presence of absence. The word “civilized” carries the trace of “barbaric.” “Normal” carries the trace of “abnormal.” “Legal” carries the trace of “illegal.” “Man” as a supposedly universal human category may carry the trace of excluded woman, animal, colonized subject, slave, or non-citizen.  
  
Trace makes binary hierarchy unstable. What a term excludes remains necessary to its meaning.  
  
**Typical sentence:** The trace is the absent other that a term needs in order to appear present. (痕迹是一个术语为了显得在场而需要的缺席他者。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Presence (在场; fr: présence)** suggests full givenness; **Trace (痕迹; fr: trace)** shows that presence is marked by absence. (在场暗示完整给予；痕迹显示在场被缺席标记。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** trace links Derrida with Heidegger’s concealment and Freud’s unconscious, but turns both toward textual and semiotic analysis. (痕迹把德里达同海德格尔的遮蔽和弗洛伊德的无意识连接起来，但把二者转向文本和符号分析。)  
  
### 19. Supplement: The Problem of the “Extra” That Reveals Lack  
  
`Supplement (补充/增补; fr: supplément)`  
**Definition:** an addition that seems secondary but reveals and displaces a lack in what was supposed to be complete. (一种看似次要的添加物，却揭示并置换了原本被认为完整之物中的缺失。)  
**Problem solved:** it exposes the instability of origin, presence, and completeness. (它揭示起源、在场和完整性的稳定性问题。)  
**Why needed:** what is called secondary often proves necessary to what claims to be primary. (被称为次要之物常常证明对自称首要之物是必要的。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing a supposedly external addition that turns out to constitute the original. (当分析一个看似外部添加物却实际上构成原初物的东西时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
A supplement is both addition and replacement. Writing is often treated as a supplement to speech: speech supposedly expresses living presence, writing merely records it. Derrida asks why speech needs writing if speech is complete. The supplement reveals lack in the origin.  
  
The same logic applies elsewhere. A constitution may need interpretation. A law may need precedent. A gender identity may need repeated performance. A national identity may need ceremonies and borders. These supplements show that the supposed origin is not self-sufficient.  
  
**Typical sentence:** The supplement appears as an addition to fullness, but reveals that fullness was never complete. (补充看似添加于充盈之上，却揭示所谓充盈从未完整。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Addition (添加; en: addition)** merely adds to something; **Supplement (补充; fr: supplément)** both adds to and destabilizes what it supplements. (添加只是加上某物；补充既添加于某物，又动摇被补充者。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** supplement becomes a tool for analyzing institutions, texts, bodies, laws, and identities that depend on what they subordinate. (补充成为分析制度、文本、身体、法律和身份的工具，显示它们依赖其所贬低之物。)  
  
### 20. Deconstruction: The Problem of Unstable Hierarchies  
  
`Deconstruction (解构; fr: déconstruction)`  
**Definition:** a reading practice that exposes how conceptual oppositions depend on exclusions, traces, supplements, and instabilities that they cannot master. (一种阅读实践，它揭示概念对立如何依赖其无法掌控的排除、痕迹、补充和不稳定性。)  
**Problem solved:** it shows that philosophical hierarchies are not self-grounding. (它显示哲学等级结构并非自我奠基。)  
**Why needed:** many concepts stabilize themselves by subordinating what they secretly require. (许多概念通过贬低其暗中需要之物来稳定自身。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing binary oppositions, suppressed terms, contradictions, textual tensions, or claims of pure origin and presence. (当分析二元对立、被压制项、矛盾、文本张力或纯粹起源与在场主张时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Deconstruction is not destruction. It does not simply tear down a text. It reads closely to show how the text’s own terms produce tensions that exceed its explicit claims.  
  
A deconstructive reading often proceeds in three movements:  
  
First, identify a hierarchy: speech over writing, presence over absence, reason over body, nature over culture, man over woman, literal over metaphorical. (第一，识别等级：言语高于书写、在场高于缺席、理性高于身体、自然高于文化、男人高于女人、字面高于隐喻。)  
  
Second, show that the privileged term depends on the subordinated term. (第二，显示被优先化的术语依赖被贬低的术语。)  
  
Third, show that the opposition cannot remain stable in its original form. (第三，显示这一对立无法以原形式保持稳定。)  
  
**Typical sentence:** Deconstruction does not stand outside a text to refute it; it follows the text’s own logic until its hierarchy becomes unstable. (解构并不站在文本外部反驳它；它追随文本自身逻辑，直到其等级结构变得不稳定。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Critique (批判; de: Kritik)** often evaluates a position by standards; **Deconstruction (解构; fr: déconstruction)** exposes internal dependence and instability within the position’s own terms. (批判常按标准评价一个立场；解构则揭示该立场自身术语内部的依赖与不稳定。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** deconstruction extends Heidegger’s destruction of metaphysics into a textual analysis of presence, hierarchy, and exclusion. (解构把海德格尔对形而上学的拆毁扩展为关于在场、等级和排除的文本分析。)  
  
### 21. Logocentrism: The Problem of Presence and Voice  
  
`Logocentrism (逻各斯中心主义; el: λόγος; fr: logocentrisme)`  
**Definition:** the tendency in Western metaphysics to privilege logos, presence, speech, reason, origin, or self-identical meaning. (西方形而上学中优先化逻各斯、在场、言语、理性、起源或自我同一意义的倾向。)  
**Problem solved:** it names the metaphysical desire for final grounding and full presence. (它命名形而上学对最终根据和完整在场的欲望。)  
**Why needed:** many philosophical systems rely on a privileged center that secures meaning. (许多哲学系统依赖一个特权中心来保证意义。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing appeals to pure reason, original speech, immediate presence, self-evident meaning, or ultimate foundation. (当分析对纯理性、原初言语、直接在场、自明意义或终极根据的诉求时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Logocentrism does not mean valuing reason in any ordinary sense. It names a structural tendency: the search for a final term that stabilizes meaning and hierarchy. Derrida connects logocentrism with **Phonocentrism (语音中心主义; fr: phonocentrisme)**, the privileging of speech over writing because speech seems closer to living presence and intention.  
  
Deconstruction asks whether this privilege can be maintained.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Logocentrism seeks a center that would make meaning fully present and finally grounded. (逻各斯中心主义寻求一个能够使意义完全在场并最终奠基的中心。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Logos (逻各斯; el: λόγος)** in Greek can mean speech, reason, account, relation, and order; **Logocentrism (逻各斯中心主义; fr: logocentrisme)** is Derrida’s critical term for the metaphysical privileging of grounding presence. (希腊 Logos 可指言说、理性、说明、关系和秩序；逻各斯中心主义则是德里达用来批判形而上学优先化奠基性在场的术语。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** logocentrism links post-structuralism back to the Greek **Logos** and forward to critiques of metaphysics, patriarchy, colonial rationality, and textual authority. (逻各斯中心主义把后结构主义向后连接到希腊 Logos，向前连接到对形而上学、父权制、殖民理性和文本权威的批判。)  
  
### 22. Center and Play: The Problem of Structure without Final Ground  
  
`Center (中心; la: centrum; fr: centre)`  
**Definition:** the privileged point that organizes a structure while claiming to stand outside or above structural play. (一个组织结构却声称自身处于结构游戏之外或之上的特权点。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains how systems try to stabilize themselves. (它解释系统如何试图稳定自身。)  
**Why needed:** structures often depend on a center that limits movement and secures meaning. (结构常依赖一个限制运动并保证意义的中心。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing origin, foundation, author, God, reason, subject, nature, or law as stabilizing centers. (当分析起源、根据、作者、上帝、理性、主体、自然或法律作为稳定中心时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
`Play (游戏/游移; fr: jeu)`  
**Definition:** the movement, substitution, and displacement of elements within a structure once no final center fully stabilizes them. (当没有最终中心完全稳定元素时，元素在结构中的运动、替换和位移。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains meaning’s mobility after decentering. (它解释去中心化之后意义的流动性。)  
**Why needed:** if no final center closes the system, elements can shift and be reconfigured. (如果没有最终中心封闭系统，元素就会移动并被重新配置。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing instability, substitution, textual movement, reinterpretation, or the failure of final closure. (当分析不稳定、替换、文本运动、重新解释或最终封闭失败时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Derrida’s point is not that structures disappear. Rather, structures no longer receive secure closure from an unquestioned center. This creates play. Meaning can still function, but it is not finally mastered.  
  
**Typical sentence:** A center limits play by promising final stability; decentering releases the movement that the center had contained. (中心通过承诺最终稳定来限制游移；去中心化释放中心曾试图容纳的运动。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Structure (结构; fr: structure)** organizes relations; **Center (中心; fr: centre)** attempts to ground or close those relations. (结构组织关系；中心试图奠基或封闭这些关系。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** center/play analysis connects structuralism to post-structuralism. The structure remains, but its grounding center is questioned. (中心/游移分析把结构主义连接到后结构主义。结构仍在，但其奠基性中心受到质疑。)  
  
### 23. Discourse: The Problem of Meaning as Rule-Governed Practice  
  
`Discourse (话语; la: discursus; fr: discours)`  
**Definition:** a historically organized field of statements, rules, practices, institutions, and subject-positions that determines what can be said, known, and recognized. (一种历史组织起来的陈述、规则、实践、制度和主体位置场域，它决定什么能够被说、被知和被承认。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains meaning and knowledge as produced through historical rules rather than individual intention alone. (它把意义和知识解释为通过历史规则生产出来的，而不只是个体意图的产物。)  
**Why needed:** what counts as knowledge depends on rules of formation, institutions, classifications, and authorized speakers. (什么算作知识取决于形成规则、制度、分类和被授权的说话者。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing scientific fields, legal regimes, medical categories, sexuality, madness, crime, education, or administrative knowledge. (当分析科学领域、法律体制、医学类别、性、疯狂、犯罪、教育或行政知识时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
**Usage layers:**  
1. **Ordinary-language use (普通用法):** **discourse** may mean conversation, discussion, speech, or extended verbal exchange. This is not the main technical use in this chapter. (普通用法中，discourse 可指谈话、讨论、言说或较长的语言交流；这不是本章的主要技术义。)  
  
2. **Foucaultian technical use (福柯式技术用法):** **discourse** means a historically specific field of statements, rules, objects, institutions, classifications, and subject-positions that determine what can be said and known. (福柯式技术义中，话语是历史上特定的陈述、规则、对象、制度、分类和主体位置的场域，决定什么能够被说和被认识。)  
  
3. **Contemporary transferable use (当代理论泛用法):** in cultural studies, legal theory, media studies, feminism, postcolonial theory, and sociology, discourse often means a socially organized meaning-system that shapes visibility, authority, identity, and norms. (在文化研究、法理论、媒介研究、女性主义、后殖民理论和社会学中，话语常指社会组织起来的意义系统，塑造可见性、权威、身份和规范。)  
  
**Transfer rule:** use **discourse** when the issue is the rule-governed production of sayability, knowledge, objects, and subjects. Do not use it when “conversation,” “text,” “language,” “ideology,” or “narrative” is more precise. (转用规则：当问题是可说性、知识、对象和主体如何被规则化生产时，才使用 discourse。如果“谈话”“文本”“语言”“意识形态”或“叙事”更准确，就不要使用 discourse。)  
  
**Misuse warning:** **Discourse** is not merely “what people say.” (Discourse 不只是“人们说了什么”。)  
  
Discourse is not merely conversation. It is a rule-governed field of sayability and knowability. A discourse determines not only what is said, but who may speak, what counts as evidence, what categories exist, what objects appear, and what subjects are produced.  
  
This concept is strongly associated with Foucault, though it also belongs to broader post-structuralist vocabulary. It shifts analysis from signs alone to historically institutionalized systems of statements and practices.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Discourse is the field that determines what can be said, who can speak, and what can count as knowledge. (话语是决定什么能够被说、谁能够说、什么能够算作知识的场域。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Language (语言; fr: langage)** is a broad symbolic capacity or system; **Discourse (话语; fr: discours)** is a historically specific field of statements, rules, institutions, and practices. (语言是宽泛的符号能力或系统；话语是历史上特定的陈述、规则、制度和实践场域。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** discourse analysis transforms structuralism by adding history, institution, power, and subject-formation. It prepares the next stage: Foucault’s archaeology and genealogy of knowledge. (话语分析通过加入历史、制度、权力和主体形成来改造结构主义，并为下一阶段福柯的知识考古学与谱系学做准备。)  
  
### 24. Subject-Position: The Problem of Being Spoken by Discourse  
  
`Subject-Position (主体位置; fr: position de sujet)`  
**Definition:** a place within discourse from which a person can speak, be recognized, be classified, and become intelligible. (人在话语中能够说话、被承认、被分类并成为可理解者的位置。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains subjectivity as produced through symbolic and institutional positions. (它把主体性解释为通过符号和制度位置被生产出来的东西。)  
**Why needed:** people do not enter discourse as pure subjects; they are positioned as patient, citizen, criminal, student, expert, consumer, native, foreigner, man, woman, normal, deviant. (人并不是作为纯粹主体进入话语；他们被定位为病人、公民、罪犯、学生、专家、消费者、本地人、外国人、男人、女人、正常者、异常者。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing how discourse assigns identity, authority, visibility, and constraints. (当分析话语如何分配身份、权威、可见性和限制时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Subject-position does not mean personal opinion. It means the structural position from which speech becomes possible and recognizable. A doctor and patient do not speak from equivalent subject-positions inside medical discourse. A judge, defendant, witness, and lawyer do not occupy equivalent positions inside legal discourse.  
  
This explains why “voice” is never simply natural. One may speak, but not be heard as credible. One may be visible, but only as a stereotype. One may be classified before speaking.  
  
**Typical sentence:** A subject-position is the discursive place from which someone becomes speakable, visible, and governable. (主体位置是某人在话语中成为可说、可见和可治理者的位置。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Individual (个体; la: individuum)** names a person as singular entity; **Subject-Position (主体位置; fr: position de sujet)** names the discursive-institutional place through which that person is recognized. (个体命名作为单一实体的人；主体位置命名该人借以被承认的话语—制度位置。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** subject-position analysis links post-structuralism with feminism, queer theory, critical race theory, postcolonial theory, legal theory, and digital governance. (主体位置分析把后结构主义同女性主义、酷儿理论、批判种族理论、后殖民理论、法理论和数字治理连接起来。)  
  
### 25. The Tool-Map of Structuralism and Post-Structuralism  
  
Use structuralist and post-structuralist vocabulary diagnostically. The core question is usually not “what does the author intend?” but “what system, difference, code, or discourse makes this meaning possible and unstable?”  
  
**If the text analyzes how meaning is produced by signs**, look for **Sign (符号; fr: signe)**, **Signifier (能指; fr: signifiant)**, and **Signified (所指; fr: signifié)**.  
(如果文本分析意义如何由符号生产，应寻找符号、能指和所指问题。)  
  
**If the text analyzes meaning through relations**, look for **Difference (差异; fr: différence)**, **Structure (结构; fr: structure)**, and **System (系统; fr: système)**.  
(如果文本通过关系分析意义，应寻找差异、结构和系统问题。)  
  
**If the text distinguishes system from individual use**, look for **Langue (语言系统; fr: langue)** and **Parole (言语活动; fr: parole)**.  
(如果文本区分系统与个体使用，应寻找 langue 与 parole 问题。)  
  
**If the text analyzes current structure versus historical change**, look for **Synchrony (共时性; fr: synchronie)** and **Diachrony (历时性; fr: diachronie)**.  
(如果文本分析当前结构与历史变化，应寻找共时性和历时性问题。)  
  
**If the text analyzes cultural readability**, look for **Code (符码; fr: code)**, **Myth (神话; fr: mythe)**, and **Binary Opposition (二元对立; fr: opposition binaire)**.  
(如果文本分析文化可读性，应寻找符码、神话和二元对立问题。)  
  
**If the text displaces author or subject as origin**, look for **Decentering (去中心化; fr: décentrement)**, **Text (文本; fr: texte)**, and **Intertextuality (互文性; fr: intertextualité)**.  
(如果文本移置作者或主体作为起源的位置，应寻找去中心化、文本和互文性问题。)  
  
**If the text analyzes instability of meaning**, look for **Post-Structuralism (后结构主义; fr: post-structuralisme)**, **Différance (延异; fr: différance)**, **Trace (痕迹; fr: trace)**, and **Supplement (补充; fr: supplément)**.  
(如果文本分析意义的不稳定，应寻找后结构主义、延异、痕迹和补充问题。)  
  
**If the text destabilizes conceptual hierarchies**, look for **Deconstruction (解构; fr: déconstruction)**, **Logocentrism (逻各斯中心主义; fr: logocentrisme)**, **Center (中心; fr: centre)**, and **Play (游移; fr: jeu)**.  
(如果文本动摇概念等级，应寻找解构、逻各斯中心主义、中心和游移问题。)  
  
**If the text analyzes historically governed sayability**, look for **Discourse (话语; fr: discours)** and **Subject-Position (主体位置; fr: position de sujet)**.  
(如果文本分析历史地被规制的可说性，应寻找话语和主体位置问题。)  
  
### 26. The Genealogical Point of Part 12  
  
Structuralism and post-structuralism transform the problem of philosophical language. Greek philosophy made **Logos** into a grammar of reasoned account. Latin metaphysics stabilized meaning through substance, essence, law, and order. Early modern philosophy tied meaning to the subject and representation. Analytic philosophy disciplined meaning through propositions, reference, and truth-conditions. Hermeneutics situated meaning in tradition and horizon.  
  
Structuralism says: **meaning is produced by systems of difference.**  
(结构主义说：意义由差异系统生产。)  
  
Post-structuralism says: **because meaning is produced by difference, it never becomes fully present, final, or self-identical.**  
(后结构主义说：正因为意义由差异生产，它永远不能成为完全在场、最终确定或自我同一的意义。)  
  
The guiding thesis is:  
  
**Structuralist and post-structuralist language turns meaning into a problem of differential systems and unstable signification: to understand a concept, text, institution, or identity is to ask what system of signs makes it intelligible, what oppositions organize it, what exclusions stabilize it, and where its meaning begins to slip.**  
(结构主义与后结构主义语言把意义转化为差异系统与不稳定表意的问题：理解一个概念、文本、制度或身份，就是追问什么符号系统使它成为可理解之物，什么对立组织它，什么排除稳定它，以及它的意义在哪里开始滑动。)  
  
This grammar prepares the next stage directly. Foucault will turn structural and post-structural insights toward **Archaeology**, **Genealogy**, **Discourse**, **Power/Knowledge**, **Discipline**, **Biopolitics**, and **Subjectivation**. Derrida will continue to analyze trace, différance, supplement, and deconstruction. Feminist, queer, postcolonial, legal, and media theory will use these tools to analyze how bodies, identities, nations, laws, archives, platforms, and data systems become readable and governable.  
  
The structuralist/post-structuralist question remains one of the strongest tools for philosophical reading:  
  
**What system of differences makes this meaning possible, and what instability does that same system conceal?**  
(什么差异系统使这个意义成为可能？而同一个系统又遮蔽了什么不稳定性？)  
  
## Part 13. Foucault: Archaeology, Genealogy, Power/Knowledge  
  
This chapter explains **Michel Foucault** as the point where several previous lines converge: **Nietzschean genealogy**, **structuralist discourse analysis**, **critical suspicion**, and **historical epistemology**. Foucault does not mainly ask whether a proposition is true, whether consciousness intends an object, or whether a text has a hidden meaning. His central question is: **under what historical conditions can something become an object of knowledge, a target of power, and a form of subjectivity?** (在什么历史条件下，某物能够成为知识对象、权力目标和主体形式？)  
  
The central vocabulary is **Archaeology**, **Archive**, **Statement**, **Discursive Formation**, **Episteme**, **Discontinuity**, **Genealogy**, **Power**, **Power/Knowledge**, **Regime of Truth**, **Discipline**, **Panopticism**, **Normalization**, **Examination**, **Docile Body**, **Biopolitics**, **Population**, **Governmentality**, **Apparatus**, **Subjectivation**, and **Technologies of the Self**. **Archaeology** analyzes the underlying rules of discourse in a given epoch, while **episteme** names the unconscious framework of knowledge at a historical moment. **Power/Knowledge** names the inseparability of power relations and knowledge production. Foucault’s conceptual core is that power is not primarily repressive but productive: it produces subjects, knowledges, behaviors, and bodies through apparatuses such as the prison, clinic, school, confession, and census.  
  
The operational function of this chapter is exact: use Foucauldian vocabulary when the problem is **how truth, subjectivity, normality, and institutions are historically produced through relations of knowledge and power**. (当问题是“真理、主体性、正常性与制度如何通过知识—权力关系被历史地生产出来”时，应使用福柯式词汇。)  
  
### 1. The Problem-Situation: From Meaning to Conditions of Sayability  
  
Structuralism asked how signs acquire meaning inside systems of difference. Post-structuralism asked why these systems cannot finally stabilize meaning. Foucault shifts the pressure again. He asks not only how signs mean, but **how statements become sayable, knowable, classifiable, and institutionally effective**. (他不仅追问符号如何表意，而是追问陈述如何成为可说的、可知的、可分类的和具有制度效力的东西。)  
  
This is a decisive shift.  
  
The question is not only:  
  
**What does this statement mean?**  
(这个陈述意味着什么？)  
  
Nor only:  
  
**What binary opposition structures it?**  
(什么二元对立结构化了它？)  
  
But:  
  
**What historical rules allow this statement to count as knowledge, evidence, diagnosis, confession, crime, illness, sexuality, risk, or truth?**  
(什么历史规则使这个陈述能够算作知识、证据、诊断、忏悔、犯罪、疾病、性、风险或真理？)  
  
Foucault’s object is not the isolated proposition. It is the field that determines what can be said seriously, by whom, with what authority, through what institutions, and with what effects.  
  
This gives Foucauldian reading its distinctive power. A hospital record, prison file, psychiatric diagnosis, school grade, police category, census form, sexual confession, risk assessment, medical protocol, or platform data profile is not merely information. It is a point where knowledge, classification, institution, and subject formation intersect.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Foucault does not ask only whether a statement is true; he asks what historical regime makes it possible for that statement to function as truth. (福柯不只追问一个陈述是否为真；他追问什么历史体制使该陈述能够作为真理运作。)  
  
### 2. Archaeology: The Problem of Discursive Conditions  
  
`Archaeology (考古学; fr: archéologie)`  
**Definition:** a method for analyzing the historical rules that make certain statements, objects, concepts, and forms of knowledge possible. (一种分析历史规则的方法，这些规则使特定陈述、对象、概念和知识形式成为可能。)  
**Problem solved:** it moves analysis away from authorial intention, linear progress, and hidden essence toward the conditions of discourse. (它把分析从作者意图、线性进步和隐藏本质转向话语条件。)  
**Why needed:** knowledge does not emerge simply because individuals observe reality; it emerges within historically specific rules of formation. (知识并不只是因为个体观察现实而产生；它在历史特定的形成规则中产生。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing the historical conditions under which a field can define objects, authorize statements, and produce knowledge. (当分析一个领域在什么历史条件下能够定义对象、授权陈述并生产知识时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Foucauldian archaeology does not dig for a pure origin. It does not ask what the first cause of an idea was. It asks what rules made a field of knowledge possible. For example, madness, illness, sexuality, criminality, and abnormality are not simply timeless natural objects waiting to be discovered. They become thinkable and governable through discursive and institutional arrangements.  
  
Archaeology therefore changes the level of analysis. Instead of interpreting what a text secretly means, it analyzes the rules that allow texts to exist as serious statements within a domain.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Archaeology studies not the hidden meaning of discourse, but the rules that make discourse possible. (考古学研究的不是话语的隐藏意义，而是使话语成为可能的规则。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Archaeology (考古学; fr: archéologie)** differs from **Hermeneutics (解释学; de: Hermeneutik)**. Hermeneutics seeks understanding of meaning; archaeology analyzes the historical rules of statement-formation. (解释学寻求意义理解；考古学分析陈述形成的历史规则。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** archaeology continues Kant’s question of conditions, but historicizes it. The question is no longer universal conditions of possible experience, but historical conditions of possible knowledge. (考古学延续康德的条件问题，但使其历史化。问题不再是可能经验的普遍条件，而是可能知识的历史条件。)  
  
### 3. Archive: The Problem of What Can Be Said  
  
`Archive (档案; fr: archive)`  
**Definition:** not merely a collection of documents, but the historical system that governs the appearance, circulation, preservation, and authority of statements. (不仅是文献集合，而是支配陈述出现、流通、保存和获得权威的历史系统。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains why not every possible sentence can function as a serious statement in a given historical field. (它解释为什么并非每个可能句子都能在特定历史领域中作为严肃陈述运作。)  
**Why needed:** discourse is regulated by rules of sayability, visibility, classification, and authority. (话语受到可说性、可见性、分类和权威规则的规制。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing the historical field that determines what can appear as knowledge. (当分析决定什么能够作为知识出现的历史场域时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
**Usage layers:**  
1. **Ordinary-institutional use (普通制度用法):** **archive** may mean a repository of documents, records, files, images, or institutional memory. (普通制度用法中，archive 指文献、记录、文件、图像或制度记忆的保存处。)  
  
2. **Foucaultian technical use (福柯式技术用法):** in Foucault, the archive is not merely a collection of documents. It is the historical system that governs what can be said, preserved, classified, repeated, and treated as knowledge. (在福柯那里，档案不只是文献集合，而是支配什么能够被说、被保存、被分类、被重复并被视为知识的历史系统。)  
  
3. **Contemporary transferable use (当代理论泛用法):** in postcolonial theory, media studies, digital humanities, and platform studies, archive may refer to colonial records, erased memory, database structure, metadata, searchable traces, or algorithmic preservation. (在后殖民理论、媒介研究、数字人文和平台研究中，档案可指殖民记录、被抹除的记忆、数据库结构、元数据、可搜索踪迹或算法保存。)  
  
**Transfer rule:** use **archive** technically when the issue is not only stored material, but the rules of preservation, visibility, classification, retrievability, and authority. (转用规则：只有当问题不只是被保存的材料，而是保存、可见性、分类、可检索性和权威规则时，才技术性地使用 archive。)  
  
**Misuse warning:** archive is not neutral storage. It organizes memory and silence. (Archive 不是中立存储；它组织记忆，也组织沉默。)  
  
The archive is not just a library, database, or institutional storage room. It is the system that determines what can be recorded, retrieved, cited, classified, forgotten, or treated as evidence. A medical archive, legal archive, colonial archive, psychiatric archive, or platform archive does not merely preserve reality. It organizes reality into categories that can be acted upon.  
  
This matters because knowledge often begins with archival form. If a person is recorded as patient, delinquent, migrant, risk, consumer, disorder, abnormality, or data subject, the archive does more than describe. It makes a mode of governance possible.  
  
**Typical sentence:** The archive is the historical system that determines which statements can appear, endure, and count. (档案是决定哪些陈述能够出现、持续并被计入的历史系统。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Archive (档案; fr: archive)** differs from **Collection (集合; en: collection)**. A collection gathers materials; an archive governs their status, order, retrievability, and authority. (集合聚集材料；档案规制材料的地位、秩序、可检索性和权威。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** archive analysis prepares later work on colonial records, legal files, medical classification, surveillance databases, algorithmic memory, and institutional forgetting. (档案分析为后来的殖民记录、法律文件、医学分类、监控数据库、算法记忆和制度性遗忘研究做准备。)  
  
### 4. Statement: The Problem of Discursive Function  
  
`Statement (陈述; fr: énoncé)`  
**Definition:** a discursive function through which a sentence, mark, formula, chart, or classification can count as part of a field of knowledge. (一种话语功能，通过它，句子、标记、公式、图表或分类能够算作某一知识领域的一部分。)  
**Problem solved:** it distinguishes grammatical sentences from historically effective knowledge-units. (它把语法句子同历史上有效的知识单位区分开来。)  
**Why needed:** not every sentence has the same discursive status; some become evidence, diagnosis, law, record, or truth-claim. (并非每个句子都具有相同话语地位；有些成为证据、诊断、法律、记录或真理主张。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing how a linguistic or semiotic unit functions inside a discourse. (当分析一个语言或符号单位如何在话语内部运作时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
A statement is not simply a proposition. Analytic philosophy asks about truth-values and logical form. Foucault asks about discursive existence: under what rules does this utterance count as a medical fact, legal accusation, psychiatric diagnosis, economic datum, or scientific observation?  
  
For example, “this person is dangerous” can be ordinary gossip, psychiatric assessment, police intelligence, court evidence, prison classification, or algorithmic risk label. The sentence form may be similar; the statement-function differs.  
  
**Typical sentence:** A statement is a unit of discourse defined by its function within a field of knowledge. (陈述是由其在知识领域中的功能所规定的话语单位。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Proposition (命题; en: proposition)** is truth-evaluable content; **Statement (陈述; fr: énoncé)** is a discursive function governed by historical rules. (命题是可评估真假的内容；陈述是由历史规则规制的话语功能。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** statement analysis shifts attention from meaning and truth-condition to institutional-discursive function. (陈述分析把注意力从意义和真值条件转向制度—话语功能。)  
  
### 5. Discursive Formation: The Problem of Ordered Knowledge Fields  
  
`Discursive Formation (话语构型; fr: formation discursive)`  
**Definition:** a historically organized system of rules that determines how objects, concepts, subject-positions, and statements are formed within a discourse. (一种历史组织起来的规则系统，它决定对象、概念、主体位置和陈述如何在话语中形成。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains why knowledge fields have patterned regularity without needing a single author, intention, or ideology. (它解释为什么知识领域具有模式化规律，而不需要单一作者、意图或意识形态来解释。)  
**Why needed:** sciences, professions, institutions, and administrative systems organize what can be said and known. (科学、专业、制度和行政系统组织什么能够被说和被知。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing a field such as psychiatry, medicine, criminology, economics, sexuality, education, or security. (当分析精神病学、医学、犯罪学、经济学、性、教育或安全等领域时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
A discursive formation is not a worldview held by individuals. It is a system of formation rules. It determines what objects can be spoken of, what concepts can be used, what methods count, what authorities matter, and what subjects can speak.  
  
For example, “mental illness” becomes an object through institutions, classifications, professional vocabularies, clinical spaces, diagnostic practices, case histories, and treatment regimes. It is not invented out of nothing, but neither is it simply given in nature in the form in which psychiatry knows it.  
  
**Typical sentence:** A discursive formation makes some objects speakable, some concepts usable, and some authorities credible. (话语构型使某些对象成为可说的，使某些概念成为可用的，并使某些权威成为可信的。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Discourse (话语; fr: discours)** is the broader field of statements and practices; **Discursive Formation (话语构型; fr: formation discursive)** names the regular system by which that discourse organizes objects and statements. (话语是陈述和实践的广阔场域；话语构型命名该话语组织对象和陈述的规则系统。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** discursive formation joins structuralist system-analysis with historical specificity. It is structure, but not timeless structure. (话语构型把结构主义的系统分析同历史特定性结合起来。它是结构，但不是无时间的结构。)  
  
### 6. Episteme: The Problem of Historical Knowledge Conditions  
  
`Episteme (认识型/知识型; el: ἐπιστήμη; fr: épistémè)`  
**Definition:** the historical a priori that structures what can count as knowledge in a given epoch. (一种历史性的先验结构，它规定某一时代中什么能够算作知识。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains deep regularities across different knowledge fields within a historical period. (它解释一个历史时期内不同知识领域之间的深层规律性。)  
**Why needed:** an epoch can organize truth, order, classification, and representation in ways that exceed any single discipline. (一个时代能够以超出单一学科的方式组织真理、秩序、分类和表象。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing the underlying historical order that makes multiple sciences or discourses intelligible. (当分析使多个科学或话语成为可理解之物的底层历史秩序时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
**Episteme** is not simply “knowledge” in the Greek sense, though it inherits that resonance. In Foucault, it names the underlying configuration that allows knowledge to appear in certain forms. It is not a conscious theory. It is closer to a historical field of intelligibility.  
  
Foucault’s episteme names the unconscious framework of knowledge at a historical moment. This is why episteme is useful for reading entire historical periods, not just individual authors.  
  
**Typical sentence:** An episteme is the historical field that silently organizes what can count as knowledge. (认识型是默默组织什么能够算作知识的历史场域。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Epistemology (认识论; el: ἐπιστήμη + λόγος)** studies knowledge in general; **Episteme (认识型; fr: épistémè)** names a historical configuration of knowledge. (认识论一般性研究知识；认识型命名知识的历史构型。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** episteme transforms Kant’s a priori into a historical a priori. Conditions of knowledge are no longer universal and fixed; they shift across epochs. (认识型把康德的先验转化为历史先验。知识条件不再是普遍固定的，而是随时代转移。)  
  
### 7. Discontinuity: The Problem of Broken Historical Continuity  
  
`Discontinuity (断裂; fr: discontinuité)`  
**Definition:** a break or rupture in the rules, objects, concepts, and forms of knowledge that organize a historical field. (组织历史场域的规则、对象、概念和知识形式中的断裂。)  
**Problem solved:** it prevents history from being read as smooth progress or continuous development. (它防止历史被读成平滑进步或连续发展。)  
**Why needed:** fields of knowledge may change by rupture, reclassification, exclusion, and reorganization rather than gradual accumulation. (知识领域可能通过断裂、重新分类、排除和重组而变化，而不只是通过渐进积累变化。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing shifts between epistemes, regimes of knowledge, institutional forms, or classifications. (当分析认识型、知识体制、制度形式或分类之间的转变时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Foucault resists histories that tell a story of continuous human progress toward truth. The modern clinic is not simply a better version of ancient medicine. The modern prison is not simply a more humane replacement for torture. Modern sexuality is not simply the liberation of a natural truth. These formations involve new objects, new gazes, new institutions, and new forms of power.  
  
Discontinuity is therefore a discipline against retrospective comfort. It blocks the assumption that the present is the natural outcome of reason’s maturation.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Discontinuity shows that knowledge does not simply grow; it can reorganize what counts as an object, method, and truth. (断裂显示知识并不只是增长；它可能重组什么算作对象、方法和真理。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Development (发展; de: Entwicklung)** suggests unfolding continuity; **Discontinuity (断裂; fr: discontinuité)** marks historical breaks in rules of formation. (发展暗示连续展开；断裂标记形成规则中的历史中断。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** discontinuity separates Foucault from Hegelian and progressive histories. History becomes a series of formations and ruptures rather than the gradual self-realization of reason. (断裂使福柯同黑格尔式和进步主义历史区分开来。历史成为一系列构型与断裂，而非理性的渐进自我实现。)  
  
### 8. Genealogy: The Problem of Contingent Formation  
  
`Genealogy (谱系学; de: Genealogie; fr: généalogie)`  
**Definition:** a historical-critical method that traces how practices, truths, norms, and subjects are contingently formed through power relations, struggles, accidents, and institutions. (一种历史批判方法，它追踪实践、真理、规范和主体如何通过权力关系、斗争、偶然事件和制度被偶然地形成。)  
**Problem solved:** it breaks the illusion that present categories are natural, necessary, or morally pure. (它打破当前分类是自然的、必然的或道德上纯洁的幻觉。)  
**Why needed:** many modern truths hide their descent from discipline, exclusion, classification, and struggle. (许多现代真理遮蔽了其来自规训、排除、分类和斗争的来源。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing how a practice or category came to appear self-evident. (当分析一种实践或分类如何变得不言自明时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Genealogy is the Nietzschean element in Foucault. It does not seek pure origin. It seeks descent, emergence, accident, struggle, and the body. Genealogy traces the evolution of ideas, questions their natural emergence, and exposes contingent power relations shaping them.  
  
Genealogy asks uncomfortable questions:  
  
How did punishment become correction?  
(惩罚如何变成矫正？)  
  
How did sexuality become a truth of the self?  
(性如何成为自我的真理？)  
  
How did madness become psychiatric object?  
(疯狂如何成为精神病学对象？)  
  
How did population become governable?  
(人口如何成为可治理对象？)  
  
**Typical sentence:** Genealogy shows that what appears necessary was produced through contingent histories of power, knowledge, and practice. (谱系学显示，看似必然之物是通过权力、知识和实践的偶然历史被生产出来的。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Origin (起源; de: Ursprung)** suggests pure beginning; **Genealogy (谱系学; fr: généalogie)** analyzes descent, emergence, conflict, and contingency. (起源暗示纯粹开端；谱系学分析来源、涌现、冲突和偶然性。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** genealogy turns critique from judgment of ideas to history of practices. Truth is no longer analyzed only as correspondence or coherence, but as something formed in regimes of power and knowledge. (谱系学把批判从观念判断转向实践史。真理不再只作为符合或融贯被分析，而是作为在权力—知识体制中形成之物被分析。)  
  
### 9. Descent and Emergence: The Problem of Non-Pure Origins  
  
`Descent (来源/血统; de: Herkunft; fr: provenance)`  
**Definition:** the impure historical line through which a practice, value, or category is formed. (一种实践、价值或分类借以形成的不纯历史线索。)  
**Problem solved:** it replaces pure origin with mixed, bodily, institutional, and accidental formation. (它用混杂的、身体的、制度性的和偶然的形成过程取代纯粹起源。)  
**Why needed:** present concepts often hide the heterogeneous histories that produced them. (当前概念常遮蔽生产它们的异质历史。)  
**How to use:** use it when tracing the historical materials from which a norm, identity, or practice descends. (当追踪一种规范、身份或实践由哪些历史材料形成时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
`Emergence (涌现/发生; de: Entstehung; fr: émergence)`  
**Definition:** the moment or process by which a practice, norm, or object appears from struggle, force, and contingent arrangement. (一种实践、规范或对象从斗争、力量和偶然配置中出现的时刻或过程。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains historical appearance without assuming final purpose. (它在不预设最终目的的情况下解释历史出现。)  
**Why needed:** what appears is often the temporary result of conflict rather than the fulfillment of essence. (出现之物常是冲突的暂时结果，而非本质的实现。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing the conditions under which a category or institution first becomes effective. (当分析一个分类或制度在什么条件下首次变得有效时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Foucauldian genealogy uses descent and emergence to resist origin myths. A modern institution may present itself as rational, humane, scientific, or necessary. Genealogy asks what struggles, failures, accidents, classifications, and administrative needs produced it.  
  
This is especially important for moralized institutions. The prison presents itself as justice. The clinic presents itself as care. The school presents itself as education. Genealogy asks what else these institutions do.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Descent traces the impure line of formation; emergence analyzes the struggle through which something becomes effective. (来源追踪形成的不纯线索；涌现分析某物借以变得有效的斗争。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Teleology (目的论; el: τέλος)** reads history as fulfillment of a goal; **Emergence (发生; de: Entstehung)** reads history as contingent formation through force and struggle. (目的论把历史读作目标实现；发生把历史读作通过力量与斗争形成的偶然构型。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** descent and emergence convert history into critique of necessity. What exists could have been otherwise. (来源与发生把历史转化为对必然性的批判。已经存在之物本来可能以其他方式存在。)  
  
### 10. Power: The Problem of Productive Force  
  
`Power (权力; fr: pouvoir)`  
**Definition:** a relational field of forces that acts on actions, produces possibilities, forms subjects, and organizes conduct. (一种作用于行动、生产可能性、形成主体并组织行为的力量关系场。)  
**Problem solved:** it breaks the model of power as only law, prohibition, violence, or sovereign command. (它打破把权力仅理解为法律、禁止、暴力或主权命令的模型。)  
**Why needed:** modern power often works by producing capacities, norms, identities, knowledge, and self-regulation. (现代权力常通过生产能力、规范、身份、知识和自我调节而运作。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing how conduct is shaped, directed, classified, trained, normalized, or made governable. (当分析行为如何被塑造、引导、分类、训练、规范化或治理化时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Foucault’s concept of power is one of his most important contributions. Power is not a thing owned by one person and imposed on another in a simple top-down way. It is relational, capillary, productive, and strategic. It runs through institutions, practices, bodies, spaces, classifications, examinations, and self-understanding.  
  
The core point is that power is not primarily repressive but productive; it produces subjects, knowledges, behaviors, and bodies through historically situated apparatuses.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Power does not only say no; it produces subjects, norms, knowledge, and fields of possible action. (权力不只是说“不”；它生产主体、规范、知识和可能行动的场域。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Sovereign Power (主权权力; fr: pouvoir souverain)** commands, forbids, and punishes from above; **Productive Power (生产性权力; fr: pouvoir productif)** forms conduct, capacities, and subjects. (主权权力从上方命令、禁止和惩罚；生产性权力形成行为、能力和主体。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** power shifts from juridical model to productive model. The question is no longer only “who commands?” but “how are subjects, bodies, and truths produced?” (权力从法权模型转向生产模型。问题不再只是“谁命令？”，而是“主体、身体与真理如何被生产？”)  
  
### 11. Power/Knowledge: The Problem of Truth as Effective  
  
`Power/Knowledge (权力/知识; fr: savoir-pouvoir; en: power/knowledge)`  
**Definition:** the inseparable relation through which power produces knowledge and knowledge extends, refines, and legitimates power. (权力生产知识，知识又扩展、细化并合法化权力的不可分关系。)  
**Problem solved:** it rejects the idea that knowledge is simply outside power or that power is merely external to truth. (它拒绝知识简单外在于权力，或权力只是外在地作用于真理的观点。)  
**Why needed:** modern institutions govern through expertise, classification, measurement, diagnosis, and normalization. (现代制度通过专业知识、分类、测量、诊断和规范化进行治理。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing prisons, clinics, schools, psychiatry, sexuality, criminology, statistics, public health, or platform governance. (当分析监狱、诊所、学校、精神病学、性、犯罪学、统计、公共卫生或平台治理时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
**Usage layers:**  
1. **Foucaultian technical use (福柯式技术用法):** **Power/Knowledge (savoir-pouvoir / power/knowledge)** names the mutual formation of knowledge practices and power relations. It does not mean that power simply falsifies knowledge from outside. (Power/Knowledge 指知识实践与权力关系的相互形成，并不是说权力从外部简单伪造知识。)  
  
2. **Reception use (接受史用法):** in later critical theory, the term is often used to analyze expertise, classification, discipline, institutions, science, medicine, law, education, and administration. (在后来的批判理论中，该术语常用于分析专业知识、分类、规训、制度、科学、医学、法律、教育和行政管理。)  
  
3. **Contemporary transferable use (当代理论泛用法):** in current interdisciplinary writing, it may refer to how data, metrics, platforms, algorithms, policy categories, or institutional expertise produce governable objects and subjects. (在当代跨学科写作中，它可指数据、指标、平台、算法、政策分类或制度性专业知识如何生产可治理的对象和主体。)  
  
**Transfer rule:** use this term only when knowledge-production and power-relation are structurally connected. Do not use it merely to say “knowledge is biased” or “truth is propaganda.” (转用规则：只有当知识生产和权力关系在结构上相互连接时，才使用这个术语。不要仅用它表示“知识有偏见”或“真理是宣传”。)  
  
**Misuse warning:** **Power/Knowledge** does not mean “all knowledge is false.” (Power/Knowledge 不等于“所有知识都是假的”。)  
  
Power relations and knowledge production are inseparable, and what counts as truth is shaped by power structures.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Power/knowledge means that modern power governs by producing the knowledge through which its objects become visible and manageable. (权力/知识意味着现代权力通过生产知识来治理，而这些知识使其对象变得可见和可管理。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Ideology (意识形态; de: Ideologie)** often suggests distorted belief masking reality; **Power/Knowledge (权力/知识; fr: savoir-pouvoir; en: power/knowledge)** analyzes the productive formation of truth-effects within institutions. (意识形态常暗示遮蔽现实的扭曲信念；权力/知识分析制度中真理效果的生产性形成。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** power/knowledge moves beyond the simple opposition between true science and false ideology. It asks how scientific, administrative, and expert knowledge become instruments and effects of power. (权力/知识超出真实科学与虚假意识形态之间的简单对立，追问科学、行政与专业知识如何成为权力的工具和效果。)  
  
### 12. Regime of Truth: The Problem of Authorized Truth  
  
`Regime of Truth (真理体制; fr: régime de vérité)`  
**Definition:** the institutional and discursive arrangement that determines what counts as true, who can speak truth, how truth is verified, and what effects truth has. (决定什么算作真、谁能够说真、真如何被验证以及真产生何种效果的制度与话语配置。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains truth as socially and institutionally organized without reducing it to individual opinion. (它把真理解释为社会和制度组织的东西，而不把它化约为个人意见。)  
**Why needed:** every society has procedures for producing, authorizing, circulating, and sanctioning truth. (每个社会都有生产、授权、流通和制裁真理的程序。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing courts, science, medicine, media, education, bureaucracy, or data systems as truth-producing institutions. (当把法院、科学、医学、媒体、教育、官僚制或数据系统作为真理生产制度来分析时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
A regime of truth is not a simple conspiracy. It is a set of procedures. Who counts as expert? What counts as evidence? Which instruments produce valid observations? Which institutions certify truth? Which forms of speech are excluded as madness, bias, ignorance, activism, superstition, or misinformation?  
  
This concept is crucial for contemporary analysis. Search engines, academic peer review, courts, hospitals, intelligence agencies, platforms, and statistical agencies all participate in regimes of truth. They do not merely transmit truth. They format it.  
  
**Typical sentence:** A regime of truth organizes the production, authorization, circulation, and effects of truth. (真理体制组织真理的生产、授权、流通和效果。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Truth (真理; el: ἀλήθεια; la: veritas)** can name correspondence, disclosure, or validity; **Regime of Truth (真理体制; fr: régime de vérité)** names the historical system through which truth is produced and authorized. (真理可以指符合、开显或有效性；真理体制命名真理被生产和授权的历史系统。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** truth becomes an institutional event, not only a logical property or metaphysical disclosure. (真理成为制度性事件，而不只是逻辑属性或形而上学开显。)  
  
### 13. Discipline: The Problem of Training Bodies  
  
`Discipline (规训; fr: discipline)`  
**Definition:** a form of power that trains individual bodies through surveillance, examination, spatial distribution, time control, exercise, ranking, and normalization. (一种通过监视、考试、空间分配、时间控制、训练、排名和规范化来训练个体身体的权力形式。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains modern control below the level of sovereign law and spectacular punishment. (它解释低于主权法律和景观式惩罚层面的现代控制。)  
**Why needed:** modern institutions produce useful, obedient, measurable, and improvable bodies. (现代制度生产可用、服从、可测量和可改进的身体。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing schools, prisons, barracks, factories, hospitals, offices, platforms, or self-optimization culture. (当分析学校、监狱、军营、工厂、医院、办公室、平台或自我优化文化时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Discipline is not merely punishment. It is training. It organizes space, time, gesture, attention, posture, performance, and comparison. It produces the individual as an object of knowledge and intervention.  
  
Disciplinary society shapes bodies, time, emotion, ability, and self-understanding through schools, hospitals, prisons, companies, families, platforms, and self-optimization culture. It works through techniques such as timetables, seating, exams, files, rankings, physical checks, scores, performance metrics, monitoring, platform data, self-management, and standards of normality.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Discipline produces individuals by making bodies visible, comparable, trainable, and correctable. (规训通过使身体可见、可比较、可训练和可矫正来生产个体。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Punishment (惩罚; la: poena)** responds to an offense; **Discipline (规训; fr: discipline)** continuously forms conduct before, during, and after offense. (惩罚回应违法；规训在违法之前、之中和之后持续形成行为。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** discipline changes political theory. Power is no longer located only in law, state, or sovereign command; it is distributed through everyday institutional techniques. (规训改变政治理论。权力不再只位于法律、国家或主权命令中，而是分布在日常制度技术中。)  
  
### 14. Panopticism: The Problem of Internalized Visibility  
  
`Panopticism (全景敞视主义; fr: panoptisme)`  
**Definition:** a form of power in which possible visibility induces self-regulation. (一种权力形式，其中可能被看见的状态诱发自我规制。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains how surveillance can operate without constant physical force. (它解释监视如何在没有持续物理强制的情况下运作。)  
**Why needed:** modern power often works when subjects monitor themselves because they may be observed. (现代权力常在人们因为可能被观察而自我监控时运作。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing surveillance, schools, workplaces, prisons, platforms, metrics, dashboards, or behavioral scoring. (当分析监视、学校、工作场所、监狱、平台、指标、仪表盘或行为评分时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
The Panopticon is not important only as prison architecture. It is a diagram of power. If one may be observed at any time, one begins to behave as if observed. The gaze becomes internalized.  
  
Contemporary forms include CCTV, workplace analytics, learning management systems, social media visibility, credit scores, health tracking, productivity dashboards, and reputation systems. These systems do not need continuous punishment. They produce anticipatory self-management.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Panopticism works when the possibility of being seen makes subjects regulate themselves. (全景敞视主义在“可能被看见”使主体自我规制时运作。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Surveillance (监视; fr: surveillance)** is observation; **Panopticism (全景敞视主义; fr: panoptisme)** is the power-effect by which possible observation produces self-discipline. (监视是观察；全景敞视主义是可能观察生产自我规训的权力效果。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** panopticism moves power analysis from visible violence to visibility itself. To be seen, recorded, ranked, and compared is already to be governed. (全景敞视主义把权力分析从可见暴力转向可见性本身。被看见、记录、排名和比较已经是在被治理。)  
  
### 15. Examination: The Problem of Knowledge through Evaluation  
  
`Examination (考试/检查; fr: examen)`  
**Definition:** a disciplinary technique combining surveillance and normalization by making individuals visible, comparable, recordable, and correctable. (一种把监视与规范化结合起来的规训技术，它使个体可见、可比较、可记录和可矫正。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains how institutions produce knowledge about individuals while ranking and shaping them. (它解释制度如何在生产关于个体的知识的同时对个体进行排名和塑造。)  
**Why needed:** modern institutions govern through records, tests, files, grades, diagnoses, audits, and metrics. (现代制度通过记录、测试、档案、成绩、诊断、审计和指标进行治理。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing schools, medicine, psychiatry, prisons, HR systems, testing regimes, performance review, or platform scores. (当分析学校、医学、精神病学、监狱、人力资源系统、测试制度、绩效评估或平台评分时，应使用这一概念。)
