The examination is a small technical form with enormous social consequences. It produces a case. It records deviation. It compares individuals against norms. It turns a person into a file, profile, diagnosis, score, transcript, risk category, or developmental trajectory.  
  
This is why examination links knowledge and power. It does not only discover what someone is. It helps make someone into an object that can be treated, corrected, advanced, excluded, punished, or optimized.  
  
**Typical sentence:** The examination individualizes by recording, comparing, and normalizing. (考试/检查通过记录、比较和规范化来个体化。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Test (测试; en: test)** may measure performance; **Examination (考试/检查; fr: examen)** in Foucault names a power-knowledge technique that produces the individual as a case. (测试可以测量表现；福柯意义上的考试/检查是一种权力—知识技术，它把个体生产为案例。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** examination becomes the basic mechanism of modern institutional individuality. The modern individual is not only free; it is documented. (考试/检查成为现代制度性个体的基本机制。现代个体不只是自由的；它是被记录的。)  
  
### 16. Normalization: The Problem of the Norm  
  
`Normalization (规范化/正常化; fr: normalisation)`  
**Definition:** the process by which conduct, bodies, abilities, desires, and populations are measured, compared, corrected, and organized around norms. (行为、身体、能力、欲望和人口围绕规范被测量、比较、矫正和组织的过程。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains power that operates through standards rather than only laws. (它解释通过标准而非仅通过法律运作的权力。)  
**Why needed:** modern institutions govern by distinguishing normal, abnormal, risky, delayed, excellent, deficient, healthy, deviant, and optimized. (现代制度通过区分正常、异常、风险、迟缓、优秀、缺陷、健康、偏差和优化来治理。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing medicine, education, psychology, sexuality, disability, risk, productivity, or social metrics. (当分析医学、教育、心理学、性、残障、风险、生产率或社会指标时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Normalization differs from law. Law divides permitted and forbidden. Norms create distributions, averages, deviations, and corrective trajectories. A person can be legal but abnormal, compliant but underperforming, healthy but suboptimal, free but constantly measured.  
  
This is crucial for modern power. The norm is softer than law, but often more pervasive. It does not merely punish disobedience. It produces aspiration: be healthier, more productive, more disciplined, more emotionally regulated, more employable, more visible, more optimized.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Normalization governs by producing standards against which individuals and populations are measured. (规范化通过生产标准来治理，个体和人口都被这些标准测量。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Law (法律; la: lex; fr: loi)** prohibits and permits; **Norm (规范; la: norma; fr: norme)** measures, compares, ranks, and corrects. (法律禁止和允许；规范测量、比较、排序和矫正。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** normalization shifts social critique from rights violation alone to the production of normality itself. (规范化把社会批判从单纯权利侵犯转向正常性本身的生产。)  
  
### 17. Docile Body: The Problem of Useful Obedience  
  
`Docile Body (驯顺身体; fr: corps docile)`  
**Definition:** a body made useful, trained, obedient, and efficient through disciplinary techniques. (通过规训技术被变得有用、受训练、服从且高效的身体。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains how power works directly on bodies without appearing only as violence. (它解释权力如何直接作用于身体，而不只是表现为暴力。)  
**Why needed:** modern institutions require bodies that can be timed, placed, corrected, examined, exercised, and optimized. (现代制度需要能够被计时、安置、矫正、检查、训练和优化的身体。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing classrooms, military drill, workplace discipline, hospital routines, athletic training, platform labor, or self-tracking. (当分析教室、军训、工作场所纪律、医院流程、运动训练、平台劳动或自我追踪时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
The docile body is not simply a passive body. It is productive. It can work, learn, move, perform, respond, obey, improve, and self-correct. This is precisely why it is valuable to modern institutions.  
  
Modern power does not only break bodies. It trains them. It makes them capable in institutionally useful ways.  
  
**Typical sentence:** A docile body is a body made useful through obedience and obedient through usefulness. (驯顺身体是通过服从而变得有用、并通过有用而变得服从的身体。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Coerced Body (被强制身体; en: coerced body)** is forced externally; **Docile Body (驯顺身体; fr: corps docile)** is trained to function within norms. (被强制身体受到外部强迫；驯顺身体被训练为在规范内运作。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** the body becomes a political surface. Politics is not only about law and sovereignty; it is also about posture, time, gesture, attention, habit, and capacity. (身体成为政治表面。政治不只是法律和主权，也涉及姿势、时间、动作、注意力、习惯和能力。)  
  
### 18. Apparatus: The Problem of Heterogeneous Power Assemblages  
  
`Apparatus (装置; fr: dispositif)`  
**Definition:** a heterogeneous ensemble of discourses, institutions, laws, architectures, administrative measures, scientific statements, moral norms, and technical practices organized around a strategic function. (由话语、制度、法律、建筑、行政措施、科学陈述、道德规范和技术实践构成的异质集合，它围绕某种战略功能组织起来。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains how power operates through mixed arrangements rather than discourse alone. (它解释权力如何通过混合配置运作，而不只是通过话语运作。)  
**Why needed:** modern governance combines buildings, forms, experts, categories, laws, technologies, and habits. (现代治理结合建筑、表格、专家、分类、法律、技术和习惯。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing prisons, sexuality, public health, security, education, welfare, borders, platforms, or data infrastructures. (当分析监狱、性、公共卫生、安全、教育、福利、边境、平台或数据基础设施时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
The apparatus is broader than discourse. A prison is not only a discourse about criminality. It is architecture, schedule, surveillance, files, guards, laws, criminology, psychology, labor, punishment, reform, and classification. A platform is not only code. It is interface, data, business model, moderation policy, recommendation logic, user norms, advertising, metrics, and identity categories.  
  
This term is useful because it prevents reduction. Modern power rarely has one form. It is assembled.  
  
**Typical sentence:** An apparatus is a strategic arrangement of discourse, institution, technique, space, and practice. (装置是话语、制度、技术、空间和实践的战略性配置。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Discourse (话语; fr: discours)** concerns rule-governed statements and knowledge; **Apparatus (装置; fr: dispositif)** includes discourse plus institutions, spaces, laws, technologies, and practices. (话语关涉受规则支配的陈述与知识；装置包括话语，也包括制度、空间、法律、技术和实践。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** apparatus analysis prepares contemporary studies of infrastructure, platforms, borders, security regimes, medical systems, and algorithmic governance. (装置分析为当代基础设施、平台、边境、安全体制、医学系统和算法治理研究做准备。)  
  
### 19. Biopolitics: The Problem of Governing Life  
  
`Biopolitics (生命政治; fr: biopolitique)`  
**Definition:** the form of modern power that takes life, population, health, birth, death, sexuality, race, risk, and biological processes as objects of governance. (一种现代权力形式，它把生命、人口、健康、出生、死亡、性、种族、风险和生物过程作为治理对象。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains how modern power governs populations rather than only territories or legal subjects. (它解释现代权力如何治理人口，而不只是治理领土或法律主体。)  
**Why needed:** modern states and institutions manage life through statistics, public health, demography, insurance, epidemiology, security, welfare, and risk. (现代国家和制度通过统计、公共卫生、人口学、保险、流行病学、安全、福利和风险来管理生命。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing population policy, public health, sexuality, race, reproduction, pandemics, welfare, migration, risk, or demographic governance. (当分析人口政策、公共卫生、性、种族、生育、疫情、福利、移民、风险或人口治理时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Biopolitics follows discipline but does not replace it. Discipline targets individual bodies. Biopolitics targets population processes. The distinction is clear: disciplinary power acts on individual bodies; biopolitics addresses population life, including education levels, mortality, birth rates, infectious disease, longevity, public health, crime rates, recidivism, family reproduction, population structure, aging, labor supply, and ethnic composition.  
  
Biopolitics is not simply care and not simply oppression. It often appears as protection: public health, welfare, safety, longevity, fertility, productivity. But these forms of care also classify, rank, exclude, and manage.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Biopolitics governs not only what subjects may do, but how populations live, reproduce, become healthy, become risky, and die. (生命政治治理的不只是主体可以做什么，也治理人口如何生活、繁殖、变得健康、变成风险以及死亡。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Discipline (规训; fr: discipline)** individualizes bodies; **Biopolitics (生命政治; fr: biopolitique)** regulates populations. (规训个体化身体；生命政治调节人口。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** political theory moves from sovereignty over territory to administration of life. Life itself becomes a political object. (政治理论从对领土的主权转向对生命的管理。生命本身成为政治对象。)  
  
### 20. Population: The Problem of Statistical Collectivity  
  
`Population (人口; fr: population)`  
**Definition:** a collective biological-social object made knowable and governable through statistics, demography, risk, health, and security. (一种通过统计、人口学、风险、健康和安全而变得可知和可治理的生物—社会集合对象。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains how modern power governs collective processes rather than only individual conduct. (它解释现代权力如何治理集体过程，而不只是治理个体行为。)  
**Why needed:** birth rates, death rates, disease rates, unemployment, migration, crime, fertility, and longevity require population-level knowledge. (出生率、死亡率、疾病率、失业、移民、犯罪、生育和寿命都需要人口层面的知识。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing statistics, public policy, risk groups, epidemiology, demography, social insurance, or security governance. (当分析统计、公共政策、风险群体、流行病学、人口学、社会保险或安全治理时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Population is not simply many people. It is a constructed object of knowledge. It appears when human beings are aggregated, counted, averaged, compared, and managed as a living mass.  
  
This is why statistics is politically powerful. It does not merely describe society. It makes society governable through rates, trends, distributions, targets, and interventions.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Population is the collective object through which life becomes calculable and governable. (人口是生命变得可计算和可治理的集合对象。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **People (人民; fr: peuple)** is a political category; **Population (人口; fr: population)** is an administrative and biopolitical category. (人民是政治分类；人口是行政和生命政治分类。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** the subject of power changes from the juridical person to the statistical population. Modern governance increasingly acts through averages, risks, and distributions. (权力对象从法权人格转向统计人口。现代治理越来越通过平均数、风险和分布来行动。)  
  
### 21. Governmentality: The Problem of Conducting Conduct  
  
`Governmentality (治理术/治理理性; fr: gouvernementalité)`  
**Definition:** the rationality and techniques through which conduct is directed, from state administration to self-management. (行为被引导的理性与技术，从国家行政到自我管理都包括在内。)  
**Problem solved:** it expands power analysis beyond the state to the conduct of conduct. (它把权力分析从国家扩展到对行为的引导。)  
**Why needed:** modern power governs by shaping choices, environments, incentives, risks, norms, and self-understanding. (现代权力通过塑造选择、环境、激励、风险、规范和自我理解来治理。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing liberalism, neoliberalism, policy, management, risk, security, self-optimization, or responsibilization. (当分析自由主义、新自由主义、政策、管理、风险、安全、自我优化或责任化时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Governmentality is one of Foucault’s most flexible later concepts. It asks how subjects are governed not only by commands but by being encouraged to govern themselves. A neoliberal subject, for example, may experience itself as free, entrepreneurial, responsible, flexible, and self-investing while being governed through markets, metrics, competition, and risk transfer.  
  
This makes governmentality especially useful for analyzing contemporary life: wellness culture, productivity systems, career platforms, financial self-management, lifestyle medicine, education rankings, credit scoring, and algorithmic recommendation.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Governmentality governs by shaping how subjects conduct themselves. (治理术通过塑造主体如何引导自身行为来治理。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Government (政府/治理; fr: gouvernement)** can mean state administration; **Governmentality (治理术; fr: gouvernementalité)** names the broader rationality of conducting conduct. (政府/治理可以指国家行政；治理术命名更广泛的“引导行为”的理性。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** power analysis moves from repression to self-formation. Subjects are governed through their freedom, not only against it. (权力分析从压制转向自我形成。主体通过其自由被治理，而不只是被反自由地治理。)  
  
### 22. Subjectivation: The Problem of Becoming a Subject  
  
`Subjectivation (主体化; fr: subjectivation)`  
**Definition:** the process through which human beings are formed as subjects: classified, governed, recognized, disciplined, and invited to understand themselves in certain ways. (人被形成为主体的过程：被分类、治理、承认、规训，并被邀请以特定方式理解自身。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains subjectivity as produced rather than simply given. (它把主体性解释为被生产出来的，而非简单给定的东西。)  
**Why needed:** subjects are formed through discourse, power, institutions, norms, practices, and self-relations. (主体通过话语、权力、制度、规范、实践和自我关系被形成。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing identity, confession, diagnosis, gender, sexuality, citizenship, criminality, expertise, or self-management. (当分析身份、忏悔、诊断、性别、性、公民身份、犯罪性、专业知识或自我管理时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
`Subjection / Assujettissement (臣服化/隶属化; fr: assujettissement)`  
**Definition:** the process by which a person is made subject to power, norms, authority, or institutional classification. (一个人被置于权力、规范、权威或制度分类之下的过程。)  
**How to use:** use it when the issue is not merely becoming intelligible as a subject, but being bound, governed, normalized, or made answerable to power. (当问题不只是成为可理解的主体，而是被约束、治理、正常化或被置于权力问责之下时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Foucault’s analysis often links subjectivation and assujettissement. One becomes a subject with agency and intelligibility, but this formation can also involve being subjected to power. This double structure is crucial. Foucault does not simply say power crushes subjects. Power forms the very subjects who can speak, desire, confess, resist, obey, and know themselves. It means becoming a subject with agency and intelligibility. It also means being subjected to power. This double sense is crucial. Foucault does not simply say power crushes subjects. Power forms the very subjects who can speak, desire, confess, resist, obey, and know themselves.  
  
For example, “the homosexual,” “the delinquent,” “the mentally ill,” “the normal child,” “the productive worker,” “the responsible citizen,” “the high-risk patient,” and “the entrepreneurial self” are not just labels placed on pre-existing identities. They are subject forms produced through discourse and practice.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Subjectivation is the process by which a person becomes both a subject and subjected. (主体化是一个人成为主体并同时被臣服化的过程。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Subject (主体; fr: sujet)** can mean agent or bearer of consciousness; **Subjectivation (主体化; fr: subjectivation)** names the historical process by which such a subject is formed. (主体可以指行动者或意识承担者；主体化命名这种主体被历史地形成的过程。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** the modern subject is no longer the foundation of knowledge. It becomes the product and relay of knowledge-power relations. (现代主体不再是知识的基础，而成为知识—权力关系的产物和传递点。)  
  
### 23. Confession: The Problem of Truth through Self-Disclosure  
  
`Confession (忏悔/供述; la: confessio; fr: aveu/confession)`  
**Definition:** a practice in which the subject is required or invited to disclose truth about itself. (主体被要求或邀请揭示关于自身真理的实践。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains how power produces truth through self-speech. (它解释权力如何通过自我言说生产真理。)  
**Why needed:** modern subjects are often governed not by silence, but by being made to speak about desire, guilt, trauma, sexuality, identity, and risk. (现代主体常常不是通过沉默被治理，而是通过被要求谈论欲望、罪责、创伤、性、身份和风险而被治理。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing therapy, sexuality, religion, policing, education, HR, social media, or self-tracking. (当分析治疗、性、宗教、警务、教育、人力资源、社交媒体或自我追踪时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Foucault’s analysis of sexuality famously rejects the simple “repressive hypothesis.” Modern power does not merely silence sex. It incites speech about sex: confession, diagnosis, case history, expert interpretation, pedagogy, therapy, and self-examination.  
  
Confession produces a subject who believes that truth lies deep inside and must be spoken. This is one of Foucault’s most important contributions to understanding modern selfhood.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Confession governs by making the subject speak its truth and recognize itself in that truth. (忏悔通过使主体说出自身真理并在该真理中认识自身来治理。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Silencing (沉默化; en: silencing)** prevents speech; **Confession (忏悔/供述; fr: aveu)** compels or invites speech as a truth-producing practice. (沉默化阻止言说；忏悔/供述则强制或邀请言说作为真理生产实践。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** power is no longer only censorship. It can operate by producing speech, self-knowledge, and identity. (权力不再只是审查。它可以通过生产言说、自我知识和身份来运作。)  
  
### 24. Technologies of the Self: The Problem of Self-Formation  
  
`Technologies of the Self (自我技术; fr: techniques de soi/technologies de soi)`  
**Definition:** practices through which individuals work on themselves in order to transform their conduct, body, soul, desires, or way of being. (个体作用于自身，以转化其行为、身体、灵魂、欲望或存在方式的实践。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains self-formation without reducing the subject to passive domination. (它解释自我形成，而不把主体化约为被动支配。)  
**Why needed:** subjects are formed not only by institutions acting on them, but also by practices through which they act on themselves. (主体不仅由制度作用于其身而形成，也由其作用于自身的实践形成。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing ascetic practice, confession, therapy, journaling, diet, training, meditation, education, self-tracking, productivity, or ethical self-cultivation. (当分析苦修、忏悔、治疗、日记、饮食、训练、冥想、教育、自我追踪、生产力实践或伦理自我修养时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Foucault’s later work complicates the picture of power. The subject is not merely dominated. It also forms itself through practices. Ancient ethics, Christian confession, modern therapy, productivity culture, wellness routines, and quantified-self practices all involve technologies of the self.  
  
The key question is not whether self-work is good or bad. The question is what form of subject it produces, under what norms, with what freedom, and through what relation to truth.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Technologies of the self are practices by which subjects shape themselves according to regimes of truth and norms of life. (自我技术是主体按照真理体制与生活规范塑造自身的实践。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Discipline (规训; fr: discipline)** trains subjects from institutional positions; **Technologies of the Self (自我技术; fr: techniques de soi)** involve subjects working on themselves. (规训从制度位置训练主体；自我技术则涉及主体作用于自身。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** Foucault’s later thought opens an ethics of self-formation without returning to a sovereign, pre-given subject. (福柯后期思想打开一种自我形成伦理，而不回到一个主权式、预先给定的主体。)  
  
### 25. Resistance: The Problem of Power without Outside  
  
`Resistance (抵抗; fr: résistance)`  
**Definition:** practices, refusals, counter-conducts, and struggles that arise within power relations and alter their field of force. (在权力关系内部产生并改变力量场的实践、拒绝、反行为和斗争。)  
**Problem solved:** it prevents Foucault’s theory of power from becoming total fatalism. (它防止福柯的权力理论变成完全宿命论。)  
**Why needed:** if power is relational, then where there is power there are possible points of resistance. (如果权力是关系性的，那么权力存在之处也存在抵抗的可能点。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing refusal, counter-practice, subversion, escape, reclassification, counter-knowledge, or struggles over truth. (当分析拒绝、反实践、颠覆、逃逸、重新分类、反知识或围绕真理的斗争时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Foucault does not offer a pure outside of power. That is precisely the point. Resistance does not come from a place untouched by power. It arises inside power relations, by redirecting, interrupting, reversing, or refusing them.  
  
This makes resistance local, strategic, and plural. It may take the form of counter-expertise, refusal of diagnosis, legal challenge, bodily practice, queer self-naming, abolitionist critique, data refusal, alternative archives, or new forms of collective life.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Resistance is not outside power; it is a modification of the power relation from within. (抵抗并不在权力之外；它是从内部改变权力关系。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Liberation (解放; fr: libération)** often suggests escape from power; **Resistance (抵抗; fr: résistance)** in Foucault names struggle within power relations. (解放常暗示逃离权力；福柯意义上的抵抗命名权力关系内部的斗争。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** political critique moves from final emancipation to ongoing struggle over practices, classifications, bodies, truth, and subjectivation. (政治批判从最终解放转向围绕实践、分类、身体、真理和主体化的持续斗争。)  
  
### 26. The Foucauldian Diagnostic Method  
  
Foucauldian analysis should not be used as a vague accusation that “everything is power.” That is weak. The method is more precise.  
  
A mature Foucauldian analysis asks two questions at once: do not deny an institution’s power because it helps, and do not deny its help because it has power; the mature analysis asks both what problem an institution solves and how it shapes and controls people.  
  
This double question is essential:  
  
**What problem does this apparatus solve?**  
(这个装置解决了什么问题？)  
  
**How does it produce, classify, normalize, and govern subjects?**  
(它如何生产、分类、规范化并治理主体？)  
  
For example:  
  
A school teaches literacy, but also ranks bodies, schedules attention, normalizes performance, produces records, and sorts futures.  
(学校教授读写能力，但也排列身体、安排注意力、规范表现、生产记录并分类未来。)  
  
A hospital heals, but also classifies bodies, produces medical truth, organizes dependency, defines normality, and governs risk.  
(医院治疗疾病，但也分类身体、生产医学真理、组织依赖、定义正常性并治理风险。)  
  
A platform connects users, but also captures behavior, ranks visibility, nudges desire, formats identity, and converts action into data.  
(平台连接用户，但也捕获行为、排序可见性、推动欲望、格式化身份并把行动转化为数据。)  
  
**Typical sentence:** A Foucauldian analysis asks what a practice makes possible and what kind of subject it produces. (福柯式分析追问一种实践使什么成为可能，以及它生产什么样的主体。)  
  
### 27. The Tool-Map of Foucault  
  
Use Foucauldian vocabulary diagnostically. The core question is usually not “what does this mean?” but “what makes this sayable, knowable, governable, and subject-forming?”  
  
**If the text analyzes historical conditions of knowledge**, look for **Archaeology (考古学; fr: archéologie)**, **Archive (档案; fr: archive)**, **Statement (陈述; fr: énoncé)**, **Discursive Formation (话语构型; fr: formation discursive)**, and **Episteme (认识型; fr: épistémè)**.  
(如果文本分析知识的历史条件，应寻找考古学、档案、陈述、话语构型和认识型问题。)  
  
**If the text rejects continuous progress narratives**, look for **Discontinuity (断裂; fr: discontinuité)** and **Historical A Priori (历史先验; fr: a priori historique)**.  
(如果文本拒绝连续进步叙事，应寻找断裂与历史先验问题。)  
  
**If the text analyzes contingent formation of practices**, look for **Genealogy (谱系学; fr: généalogie)**, **Descent (来源; de: Herkunft)**, and **Emergence (发生; de: Entstehung)**.  
(如果文本分析实践的偶然形成，应寻找谱系学、来源和发生问题。)  
  
**If the text analyzes truth as institutionally produced**, look for **Power/Knowledge (权力/知识; fr: savoir-pouvoir; en: power/knowledge)** and **Regime of Truth (真理体制; fr: régime de vérité)**.  
(如果文本把真理作为制度性生产来分析，应寻找权力/知识与真理体制问题。)  
  
**If the text analyzes schools, prisons, hospitals, factories, offices, or platforms**, look for **Discipline (规训; fr: discipline)**, **Panopticism (全景敞视主义; fr: panoptisme)**, **Examination (考试/检查; fr: examen)**, **Normalization (规范化; fr: normalisation)**, and **Docile Body (驯顺身体; fr: corps docile)**.  
(如果文本分析学校、监狱、医院、工厂、办公室或平台，应寻找规训、全景敞视主义、考试/检查、规范化和驯顺身体问题。)  
  
**If the text analyzes public health, reproduction, mortality, risk, race, or population policy**, look for **Biopolitics (生命政治; fr: biopolitique)** and **Population (人口; fr: population)**.  
(如果文本分析公共卫生、生育、死亡率、风险、种族或人口政策，应寻找生命政治与人口问题。)  
  
**If the text analyzes liberalism, neoliberalism, self-management, policy, or risk governance**, look for **Governmentality (治理术; fr: gouvernementalité)**.  
(如果文本分析自由主义、新自由主义、自我管理、政策或风险治理，应寻找治理术问题。)  
  
**If the text analyzes identity formation**, look for **Subjectivation (主体化; fr: subjectivation)**, **Confession (忏悔/供述; fr: aveu)**, and **Technologies of the Self (自我技术; fr: techniques de soi)**.  
(如果文本分析身份形成，应寻找主体化、忏悔/供述和自我技术问题。)  
  
**If the text analyzes institutional mixtures**, look for **Apparatus (装置; fr: dispositif)**.  
(如果文本分析制度、技术、话语和实践的混合配置，应寻找装置问题。)  
  
**If the text analyzes struggle without assuming a pure outside**, look for **Resistance (抵抗; fr: résistance)** and **Counter-Conduct (反行为; fr: contre-conduite)**.  
(如果文本分析不预设纯粹外部的斗争，应寻找抵抗与反行为问题。)  
  
### 28. The Genealogical Point of Part 13  
  
Foucault transforms the entire problem of philosophical language. Greek philosophy asked for **truth**, **being**, and **logos**. Latin metaphysics stabilized **law**, **order**, and **essence**. Early modern philosophy centered **subject**, **method**, and **representation**. Kant asked for conditions of possibility. German Idealism made reason historical. Marx and Nietzsche turned critique toward production, value, and suspicion. Phenomenology returned to givenness. Heidegger reopened Being. Analytic philosophy disciplined claims. Hermeneutics historicized understanding. Structuralism and post-structuralism made meaning a function of systems, difference, and discourse.  
  
Foucault asks:  
  
**What historical practices produce the objects, subjects, truths, and norms through which people are governed and govern themselves?**  
(什么历史实践生产了对象、主体、真理和规范，并通过它们使人被治理且自我治理？)  
  
The guiding thesis is:  
  
**Foucauldian language turns knowledge into a historical-political problem of formation: to understand a concept, institution, identity, or truth is to ask what discourse makes it sayable, what apparatus makes it effective, what power/knowledge relation makes it true, what norm makes it normal, and what subject it produces.**  
(福柯式语言把知识转化为形成过程的历史—政治问题：理解一个概念、制度、身份或真理，就是追问什么话语使其可说，什么装置使其有效，什么权力/知识关系使其为真，什么规范使其正常，以及它生产什么主体。)  
  
This grammar is indispensable for contemporary analysis. It applies to prisons, schools, clinics, sexuality, public health, race, data systems, AI classification, platform governance, border control, mental health, productivity culture, and self-optimization. It also changes the ethical question. The issue is not only whether something is true, useful, or free. The issue is also:  
  
**What kind of subject does this truth require and produce?**  
(这种真理要求并生产什么样的主体？)  
  
## Part 14. Derrida and Deconstruction: Presence, Trace, Iterability  
  
This chapter isolates **Jacques Derrida** from the broader post-structuralist field. The previous chapter introduced **différance**, **trace**, **supplement**, **deconstruction**, and **logocentrism** as general tools. This part deepens them as a method of philosophical reading. Foucault asks how discourse, institutions, power, and knowledge produce subjects and truths. Derrida asks a more textual and quasi-transcendental question: **what must a system of meaning exclude, subordinate, or defer in order to appear stable, present, and self-grounded?** (一个意义系统为了显得稳定、在场并自我奠基，必须排除、贬低或延迟什么？)  
  
The central vocabulary is **deconstruction**, **metaphysics of presence**, **logocentrism**, **phonocentrism**, **writing**, **archi-writing**, **différance**, **trace**, **supplement**, **iterability**, **context**, **signature**, **dissemination**, **pharmakon**, **undecidability**, **aporia**, **parergon**, and **justice**.  
  
The operational function is precise: use Derridean vocabulary when the problem is **not only what a text says**, but **how its stated hierarchy depends on what it excludes, and how meaning remains possible only because it is never fully present or finally closed**. (当问题不只是文本说了什么，而是其明说的等级结构如何依赖被排除之物，以及意义为何只有在永不完全在场、永不最终封闭的情况下才可能时，应使用德里达式词汇。)  
  
### 1. The Problem-Situation: Meaning Wants Presence, but Works through Difference  
  
Western metaphysics often wants meaning to be secure. It looks for an origin, ground, voice, concept, author, intention, essence, God, reason, consciousness, or Being that could finally stabilize meaning. Derrida calls this desire the **metaphysics of presence**. (西方形而上学常寻求一个能够最终稳定意义的起源、根据、声音、概念、作者、意图、本质、上帝、理性、意识或存在。德里达把这种欲望称为在场形而上学。)  
  
But language does not work by full presence. A sign means by differing from other signs. It also means by sending interpretation onward. No sign contains its full meaning inside itself. Every sign carries traces of other signs, absent terms, prior uses, future repetitions, and contexts that cannot be fully mastered.  
  
The Derridean question is therefore:  
  
**How does a text produce the effect of stable meaning while depending on unstable conditions of signification?**  
(文本如何在依赖不稳定表意条件的同时，生产稳定意义的效果？)  
  
This is not a rejection of meaning. It is a stricter analysis of meaning’s conditions. Meaning works. But it works because signs can be repeated, displaced, cited, supplemented, and interpreted beyond any single origin.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Derrida does not say that meaning disappears; he shows that meaning depends on difference, repetition, and deferral rather than full presence. (德里达并不是说意义消失了；他显示意义依赖差异、重复和延迟，而非完整在场。)  
  
### 2. Deconstruction: The Problem of Internal Instability  
  
`Deconstruction (解构; fr: déconstruction)`  
**Definition:** a close reading practice that exposes how a text’s conceptual hierarchy depends on what it excludes, subordinates, or treats as secondary. (一种细读实践，它揭示文本的概念等级如何依赖其排除、贬低或视为次要的东西。)  
**Problem solved:** it prevents philosophical systems from appearing self-grounding and stable when they depend on unstable oppositions. (它防止哲学系统在依赖不稳定对立的情况下仍显得自我奠基且稳定。)  
**Why needed:** many texts secure meaning by privileging one term over another: speech over writing, presence over absence, reason over body, nature over culture, literal over metaphorical, original over copy. (许多文本通过优先化一项来保证意义：言语高于书写、在场高于缺席、理性高于身体、自然高于文化、字面高于隐喻、原本高于复制。)  
**How to use:** use it when a text depends on a binary hierarchy that it cannot fully maintain. (当文本依赖一种自身无法完全维持的二元等级时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Deconstruction is not destruction. It is not a method for saying every text is meaningless. It is also not an external refutation. A deconstructive reading works from inside the text. It follows the text’s own distinctions until the subordinated term appears as necessary to the privileged term.  
  
For example, if a theory privileges speech because speech seems closer to living intention, deconstruction asks why speech needs signs, repeatability, absence, and difference. Those features are traditionally assigned to writing. Speech therefore already contains what it tries to subordinate.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Deconstruction shows that the term treated as secondary is often the condition of possibility for the term treated as primary. (解构显示，被视为次要的术语常常是被视为首要的术语的可能性条件。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Critique (批判; de: Kritik)** often judges a position by an external or explicit standard; **Deconstruction (解构; fr: déconstruction)** reveals instability internal to the position’s own distinctions. (批判常以外部或明确标准判断立场；解构揭示立场自身区分内部的不稳定。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** deconstruction inherits Heidegger’s destruction of metaphysics, Saussurean difference, and Nietzschean suspicion, but turns them into a rigorous textual analysis of conceptual hierarchy. (解构继承海德格尔对形而上学的拆毁、索绪尔式差异和尼采式怀疑，但把它们转化为关于概念等级的严格文本分析。)  
  
### 3. Metaphysics of Presence: The Problem of Full Ground  
  
`Metaphysics of Presence (在场形而上学; fr: métaphysique de la présence)`  
**Definition:** the philosophical tendency to privilege immediacy, origin, self-presence, voice, consciousness, essence, or full meaning as the ground of truth. (一种哲学倾向，它优先化直接性、起源、自我在场、声音、意识、本质或完整意义，并把它们作为真理根据。)  
**Problem solved:** it names the deep structure Derrida criticizes across Western thought. (它命名德里达在西方思想中批判的深层结构。)  
**Why needed:** many philosophical systems seek a final presence that would stop interpretation and stabilize meaning. (许多哲学系统寻求一种最终在场，以终止解释并稳定意义。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing appeals to pure origin, immediate intuition, living voice, self-transparent consciousness, or final foundation. (当分析对纯粹起源、直接直观、活的声音、自明意识或最终根据的诉求时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
The metaphysics of presence does not mean that presence is unreal. It means that philosophy often treats presence as self-sufficient. Derrida’s point is that presence is always marked by absence, difference, trace, and repeatability.  
  
A spoken word seems present because the speaker is there. But the word must be repeatable beyond that moment. A concept seems present to thought. But it receives meaning through differences from other concepts. A law seems authoritative. But it requires interpretation, application, precedent, and supplementation.  
  
**Typical sentence:** The metaphysics of presence seeks a meaning that would be fully present to itself and need no supplement. (在场形而上学寻求一种完全自我在场且不需要补充的意义。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Presence (在场; fr: présence)** names appearing as there; **Metaphysics of Presence (在场形而上学; fr: métaphysique de la présence)** names the philosophical privileging of presence as ground. (在场命名作为“在那里”的显现；在场形而上学命名把在场优先化为根据的哲学倾向。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** Derrida rereads the history of metaphysics as a history of attempts to secure meaning against trace, writing, absence, and difference. (德里达把形而上学史重读为试图保护意义免受痕迹、书写、缺席和差异影响的历史。)  
  
### 4. Logocentrism: The Problem of Grounding Meaning in Logos  
  
`Logocentrism (逻各斯中心主义; el: λόγος; fr: logocentrisme)`  
**Definition:** the privileging of logos, reason, speech, presence, origin, or foundational meaning as the center of thought. (对逻各斯、理性、言语、在场、起源或奠基意义的优先化。)  
**Problem solved:** it identifies the metaphysical structure that seeks a final center of meaning. (它识别寻求最终意义中心的形而上学结构。)  
**Why needed:** Western philosophy often assumes that meaning can be grounded in a pure logos that escapes textual difference. (西方哲学常假设意义能够奠基于一种逃离文本差异的纯粹逻各斯。)  
**How to use:** use it when a text treats reason, speech, consciousness, or origin as the stable center of meaning. (当文本把理性、言语、意识或起源视为意义稳定中心时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
**Logos (逻各斯; el: λόγος)** can mean speech, reason, account, ordering, or intelligible structure. Derrida does not simply reject logos. He criticizes **logocentrism**, the elevation of logos into a final authority that secures meaning.  
  
Logocentrism often works with a hierarchy: speech is closer to thought; writing is derivative. Presence is original; absence is secondary. Meaning is proper; metaphor is deviation. Deconstruction asks whether the privileged side can function without the excluded side.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Logocentrism treats meaning as if it could be secured by a central logos immune to difference and writing. (逻各斯中心主义把意义视为能够由一个不受差异和书写影响的中心逻各斯来保证。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Logos (逻各斯; el: λόγος)** is a broad Greek term for speech, reason, and account; **Logocentrism (逻各斯中心主义; fr: logocentrisme)** is the critical name for privileging logos as final ground. (Logos 是关于言说、理性和说明的宽泛希腊术语；逻各斯中心主义是把 logos 优先化为最终根据的批判性名称。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** logocentrism connects Derrida’s textual analysis to the whole history of Western metaphysics, from Plato to Husserl and Heidegger. (逻各斯中心主义把德里达的文本分析连接到从柏拉图到胡塞尔和海德格尔的整个西方形而上学史。)  
  
### 5. Phonocentrism: The Problem of Speech over Writing  
  
`Phonocentrism (语音中心主义; el: φωνή; fr: phonocentrisme)`  
**Definition:** the privileging of speech over writing because speech appears closer to presence, intention, consciousness, and living meaning. (对言语高于书写的优先化，因为言语似乎更接近在场、意图、意识和活的意义。)  
**Problem solved:** it identifies a key mechanism of logocentrism. (它识别逻各斯中心主义的一个关键机制。)  
**Why needed:** Western thought often treats writing as secondary representation of speech. (西方思想常把书写视为言语的次级表象。)  
**How to use:** use it when a text treats spoken voice as more authentic, immediate, or truthful than writing. (当文本把声音言语视为比书写更真实、直接或可信时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Speech seems present because speaker and listener share a moment. Writing seems absent because the author may be gone. Derrida reverses the assumption. Speech also depends on repeatable signs. A spoken word must be iterable. It can be misunderstood, cited, detached, repeated, and used outside its original intention. These are usually called features of writing, but they already inhabit speech.  
  
This is why writing is not merely secondary. The structure usually assigned to writing is general to signification itself.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Phonocentrism privileges speech as living presence, but speech already depends on repeatability and difference. (语音中心主义把言语优先化为活的在场，但言语已经依赖重复性与差异。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Speech (言语; fr: parole)** appears immediate; **Writing (书写; fr: écriture)** appears mediated. Derrida shows that speech itself is already mediated. (言语显得直接；书写显得中介化。德里达显示言语本身已经是中介化的。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** the critique of phonocentrism destabilizes the hierarchy between living voice and written mark. This becomes central for literary theory, legal interpretation, media theory, and philosophy of language. (对语音中心主义的批判动摇活的声音与书写标记之间的等级，并成为文学理论、法律解释、媒介理论和语言哲学的核心。)  
  
### 6. Writing and Archi-Writing: The Problem of Generalized Inscription  
  
`Writing (书写; fr: écriture)`  
**Definition:** not only graphic inscription, but the structure of repeatable marks that function beyond the immediate presence of speaker, intention, and context. (不仅是图形铭写，也是可重复标记在说话者、意图和语境的直接在场之外运作的结构。)  
**Problem solved:** it shows that signification depends on repeatability and absence. (它显示表意依赖重复性与缺席。)  
**Why needed:** meaning must survive beyond the moment of production in order to function as meaning. (意义必须能够超出生产时刻而存续，才能作为意义运作。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing signs as repeatable, detachable, iterable, and context-crossing. (当分析符号作为可重复、可脱离、可迭代并跨语境的东西时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
`Archi-Writing (原书写; fr: archi-écriture)`  
**Definition:** the general structure of difference, trace, spacing, and iterability that makes all signification possible, including speech. (使一切表意成为可能的差异、痕迹、间隔化和可迭代性的总结构，言语也包括在内。)  
**Problem solved:** it prevents writing from being treated as merely secondary to speech. (它防止书写被视为仅仅次于言语。)  
**Why needed:** speech and writing both depend on a more general structure of inscription and difference. (言语和书写都依赖一种更一般的铭写与差异结构。)  
**How to use:** use it when Derrida generalizes writing beyond physical letters to the structure of signification itself. (当德里达把书写从物理文字推广到表意结构本身时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Archi-writing does not mean the first historical writing system. It means that what metaphysics calls “writing” is not a late supplement to speech. The structure of writing—repeatability, spacing, absence, trace—is already necessary for meaning in general.  
  
This is why Derrida’s “writing” can be confusing. It is not ordinary handwriting. It is a technical term for the repeatable differential structure of signs.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Archi-writing names the general structure of trace and repeatability that makes both speech and writing possible. (原书写命名使言语与书写都成为可能的痕迹和重复性总结构。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Empirical Writing (经验书写; fr: écriture empirique)** means visible marks on a surface; **Archi-Writing (原书写; fr: archi-écriture)** means the structural condition of signification. (经验书写指表面上的可见标记；原书写指表意的结构条件。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** writing becomes a quasi-transcendental condition of meaning, not a secondary technology of recording speech. (书写成为意义的准先验条件，而不是记录言语的次级技术。)  
  
### 7. Différance: The Problem of Difference and Deferral  
  
`Différance (延异; fr: différance)`  
**Definition:** the movement by which meaning is produced through difference and deferred through chains of signs. (意义通过差异被生产，并通过符号链被延迟的运动。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains why meaning is never fully present in a single sign or moment. (它解释为什么意义从不在单一符号或时刻中完全在场。)  
**Why needed:** signs function only by differing from other signs and by referring beyond themselves. (符号只有通过不同于其他符号并指向自身之外才发挥作用。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing semantic delay, textual movement, non-final meaning, or the instability of presence. (当分析语义延迟、文本运动、非最终意义或在场不稳定时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
**Usage layers:**  
1. **Derridean technical use (德里达式技术用法):** **Différance** names the double movement by which meaning is produced through difference and deferred through temporal delay. It is neither a concept in the ordinary sense nor a stable origin. (Différance 指意义通过差异被生产、并通过时间延迟被推迟的双重运动。它既不是普通意义上的概念，也不是稳定起源。)  
  
2. **Poststructuralist reception use (后结构主义接受史用法):** différance becomes a tool for criticizing presence, origin, self-identity, fixed meaning, and metaphysical grounding. (在后结构主义接受史中，différance 成为批判在场、起源、自我同一性、固定意义和形而上学根据的工具。)  
  
3. **Contemporary transferable use (当代理论泛用法):** in literary theory, cultural theory, media theory, and legal theory, différance may help analyze unstable meaning, delayed reference, interpretive slippage, and the impossibility of final closure. (在文学理论、文化理论、媒介理论和法理论中，différance 可用于分析不稳定意义、延迟指称、解释滑移和最终封闭的不可能性。)  
  
**Transfer rule:** use **différance** only when both difference and deferral matter. If only contrast matters, “difference” is enough. (转用规则：只有当差异和延迟同时重要时，才使用 différance。如果只是对比关系，difference 已足够。)  
  
**Misuse warning:** **Différance** is not a decorative French word for “difference.” (Différance 不是 difference 的装饰性法语写法。)  
  
Différance is not simply “difference.” It also includes deferral. A sign means by not being another sign, but the meaning of the sign also requires further signs. A dictionary definition leads to more words. A legal term requires precedent, interpretation, and application. A philosophical concept requires its opposites, history, examples, and exclusions.  
  
Meaning therefore arrives only by not arriving fully.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Différance means that meaning is generated through difference and postponed through further signification. (延异意味着意义通过差异生成，并通过进一步表意而被推迟。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Difference (差异; fr: différence)** names distinction; **Différance (延异; fr: différance)** names the joint movement of distinction, deferral, spacing, and temporal delay. (差异命名区别；延异命名区别、延迟、间隔化和时间性推迟的联合运动。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** différance radicalizes structuralist difference by showing that differential meaning cannot become final self-presence. (延异激进化结构主义差异，显示差异性意义无法成为最终自我在场。)  
  
### 8. Trace: The Problem of Absence inside Presence  
  
`Trace (痕迹; fr: trace)`  
**Definition:** the mark of absent, excluded, prior, or other signs within any present meaning. (任何当前意义内部的缺席的、被排除的、先前的或他者性符号之标记。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains why no meaning is purely present or self-contained. (它解释为什么没有意义能够纯粹在场或自我封闭。)  
**Why needed:** a term means by carrying the traces of what it is not. (一个术语通过携带其所不是之物的痕迹而表意。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing how an absent or subordinated term remains active inside a privileged term. (当分析缺席或被贬低的术语如何在被优先化术语内部继续发挥作用时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
**Usage layers:**  
1. **Derridean technical use (德里达式技术用法):** **trace** names the mark of absence within presence: every sign bears relations to what it is not, what came before, and what is deferred. (在德里达那里，踪迹指在场中的不在场痕迹：每个符号都携带着同其所不是者、先前者和被延迟者的关系。)  
  
2. **Poststructuralist reception use (后结构主义接受史用法):** trace becomes a way to analyze meaning as relational, non-self-identical, historically marked, and never fully present to itself. (在后结构主义接受史中，踪迹成为分析意义之关系性、非自我同一性、历史标记性和无法完全自我在场的方式。)  
  
3. **Contemporary transferable use (当代理论泛用法):** in memory studies, media theory, postcolonial theory, and digital studies, trace may refer to residual marks, erased histories, data trails, archival remains, or signs of absent structures. (在记忆研究、媒介理论、后殖民理论和数字研究中，踪迹可指残留标记、被抹除历史、数据轨迹、档案遗存或缺席结构的迹象。)  
  
**Transfer rule:** use **trace** when presence is structured by absence, remainder, deferral, or relation to what is not immediately present. (转用规则：当在场由不在场、残余、延迟或同非当前之物的关系所结构时，才使用 trace。)  
  
**Misuse warning:** trace is not just evidence or footprint. It is a structural mark of absence within meaning. (Trace 不只是证据或脚印，而是意义内部不在场的结构性标记。)  
  
Trace is not a physical footprint only. It is the structural persistence of the other inside the same. “Civilized” carries the trace of “barbaric.” “Normal” carries the trace of “abnormal.” “Human” carries the trace of animal, machine, slave, woman, colonized subject, or excluded other, depending on the text.  
  
The trace is what prevents the privileged term from being self-sufficient.  
  
**Typical sentence:** The trace is the absent other that remains necessary to a term’s presence. (痕迹是对一个术语的在场仍然必要的缺席他者。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Presence (在场; fr: présence)** suggests full appearance; **Trace (痕迹; fr: trace)** shows that appearance is marked by absence. (在场暗示完整显现；痕迹显示显现被缺席所标记。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** trace gives deconstruction its anti-essentialist precision: an identity is never simply itself, because it is structured by what it excludes. (痕迹赋予解构反本质主义的精确性：同一性从不只是自身，因为它被其所排除之物结构化。)  
  
### 9. Supplement: The Problem of the Necessary Addition  
  
`Supplement (补充/增补; fr: supplément)`  
**Definition:** an addition that appears secondary but reveals a lack in what claimed to be complete. (一种看似次要的添加物，却揭示自称完整之物中的缺失。)  
**Problem solved:** it destabilizes the opposition between original and addition. (它动摇原初物与添加物之间的对立。)  
**Why needed:** many origins require supplements in order to function as origins. (许多起源需要补充物才能作为起源运作。)  
**How to use:** use it when a supposedly external support turns out to be necessary to the thing it supports. (当一个看似外部的支撑物显示出对其所支撑之物是必要的时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
The supplement both adds and replaces. It adds to something supposedly complete. But by being needed, it shows that the supposed completeness was never complete.  
  
Writing is a supplement to speech. Interpretation is a supplement to law. Ceremony is a supplement to authority. Repetition is a supplement to identity. The archive is a supplement to memory. If these supplements are necessary, then the original was never self-sufficient.  
  
**Typical sentence:** The supplement appears to complete what was already whole, but its necessity reveals that the whole was never whole. (补充看似完成已经完整之物，但其必要性揭示该完整者从未完整。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Addition (添加; en: addition)** simply adds; **Supplement (补充; fr: supplément)** adds while exposing lack. (添加只是加上；补充则在添加的同时揭示缺失。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** supplement logic becomes useful far beyond Derrida: law, identity, nation, gender, memory, authorship, and institutions often depend on supplements they deny needing. (补充逻辑在德里达之外也很有用：法律、身份、民族、性别、记忆、作者性和制度常依赖其否认需要的补充物。)  
  
### 10. Iterability: The Problem of Repeatable Signs  
  
`Iterability (可迭代性; la: iterare; fr: itérabilité)`  
**Definition:** the repeatability of a sign across different contexts, allowing it to function beyond its original intention or situation. (符号能够跨不同语境重复，从而在原初意图或情境之外运作的能力。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains how communication is possible and why meaning can escape control. (它解释交流如何可能，也解释意义为何可能逃离控制。)  
**Why needed:** a mark that could not be repeated would not be a sign. (一个无法被重复的标记就不能成为符号。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing citation, signature, law, ritual, promise, formula, meme, code, or institutional category. (当分析引用、签名、法律、仪式、承诺、公式、迷因、代码或制度分类时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Iterability is one of Derrida’s most powerful tools. A sign works because it can be repeated. But because it can be repeated, it can also be detached from its original context. This is not an accident or misuse. It is the condition of possibility of meaning.  
  
A signature can authorize only because it is repeatable. But for the same reason, it can be copied or forged. A law can govern only because it is repeatable across cases. But for the same reason, it must be interpreted in new situations. A promise can bind only because its words are repeatable beyond the moment of utterance. But for the same reason, its meaning can be contested.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Iterability makes signs usable across contexts, but it also prevents any context from fully controlling them. (可迭代性使符号能够跨语境使用，但也阻止任何语境完全控制符号。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Repetition (重复; fr: répétition)** can mean simple recurrence; **Iterability (可迭代性; fr: itérabilité)** means repeatability with possible alteration across contexts. (重复可以指单纯再发生；可迭代性指跨语境重复并可能发生变化。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** iterability gives deconstruction a theory of communication that is neither pure intention nor pure chaos. Meaning functions because signs repeat, and signs repeat only by being open to alteration. (可迭代性为解构提供一种既非纯意图也非纯混乱的交流理论。意义因符号重复而运作，而符号只有在向改变开放时才能重复。)  
  
### 11. Context: The Problem of Non-Saturability  
  
`Context (语境; la: contextus; fr: contexte)`  
**Definition:** the surrounding conditions that shape how a sign, statement, or act is interpreted. (塑造一个符号、陈述或行为如何被解释的周围条件。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains why signs mean differently in different situations. (它解释符号为何在不同情境中具有不同意义。)  
**Why needed:** signs are never interpreted in isolation. (符号从不被孤立解释。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing how situation, institution, speaker, genre, convention, law, or history shapes meaning. (当分析情境、制度、说话者、文类、约定、法律或历史如何塑造意义时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Derrida’s distinctive point is not that context is irrelevant. It is the opposite. Context matters so much that it can never be fully saturated. No context can be closed once and for all. There is always another relevant frame: legal, historical, textual, institutional, bodily, technological, political, or archival.  
  
This matters because appeals to “context” often try to stop interpretation. Derrida asks whether context itself is ever finally determinable.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Context determines meaning, but no context can be completely closed against further contextualization. (语境规定意义，但没有任何语境能够完全封闭而免于进一步语境化。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Contextualization (语境化; en: contextualization)** situates a sign; **Saturation of Context (语境饱和; en: saturation of context)** would mean complete closure, which Derrida contests. (语境化安置符号；语境饱和意味着完全封闭，而德里达对此提出质疑。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** context becomes unstable. It is no longer a fixed container of meaning, but an expandable chain of frames. (语境变得不稳定。它不再是意义的固定容器，而是可扩展的框架链条。)  
  
### 12. Signature: The Problem of Presence through Absence  
  
`Signature (签名; la: signatura; fr: signature)`  
**Definition:** a repeatable mark that authorizes presence in the absence of the signer. (一种可重复标记，它在签署者缺席时授权其在场。)  
**Problem solved:** it shows that authority depends on repeatable marks rather than immediate presence. (它显示权威依赖可重复标记，而非直接在场。)  
**Why needed:** legal, institutional, and personal authority often operates through marks detached from living presence. (法律、制度和个人权威常通过脱离活在场的标记运作。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing authorization, authorship, law, bureaucracy, identity, authenticity, or forgery. (当分析授权、作者性、法律、官僚制、身份、真实性或伪造时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
A signature works only if it can be recognized again. But if it can be recognized again, it can also be detached from the original act. It can be copied, cited, forged, scanned, automated, stamped, or digitally reproduced.  
  
Thus the signature exposes a general structure: authority depends on iterability, and iterability opens the possibility of misfire.  
  
**Typical sentence:** A signature authorizes by repeating the signer’s presence in their absence. (签名通过在签署者缺席时重复其在场来授权。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Presence of the Signer (签署者在场; en: presence of the signer)** is bodily or intentional presence; **Signature (签名; fr: signature)** is iterable authorization in absence. (签署者在场是身体或意图的在场；签名是在缺席中的可迭代授权。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** signature analysis connects deconstruction to law, bureaucracy, authorship, digital identity, cryptographic authority, and institutional trust. (签名分析把解构连接到法律、官僚制、作者性、数字身份、密码学授权和制度信任。)  
  
### 13. Dissemination: The Problem of Non-Unitary Meaning  
  
`Dissemination (播撒/散播; fr: dissémination)`  
**Definition:** the dispersal of meaning into multiple paths that cannot be gathered back into one final, unified sense. (意义散入多条路径，无法被重新收束为一个最终统一意义。)  
**Problem solved:** it challenges the idea that interpretation can always return meaning to a single center. (它挑战解释总能把意义带回单一中心的想法。)  
**Why needed:** signs generate multiple effects across contexts, texts, and readings. (符号在不同语境、文本和阅读中产生多重效果。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing plural meaning that is not reducible to ambiguity solvable by context. (当分析无法被语境解决的多重意义时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Dissemination is stronger than ordinary ambiguity. Ambiguity may have two possible meanings, and context may decide. Dissemination means meaning spreads without final gathering. The sign produces effects that cannot be mastered by authorial intention or one interpretive frame.  
  
This is especially important for literature, law, scripture, political slogans, and philosophical concepts. These forms travel. Their meanings do not remain obedient to origin.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Dissemination names the spreading of meaning beyond final return to a single governing sense. (播撒命名意义扩散到无法最终回归单一主导意义的状态。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Ambiguity (歧义; fr: ambiguïté)** may be resolved by choosing between meanings; **Dissemination (播撒; fr: dissémination)** resists final unification of meaning. (歧义可能通过在多个意义中选择而解决；播撒则抵抗意义的最终统一。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** dissemination radicalizes textual plurality. It makes reading a field of controlled instability rather than extraction of a hidden single meaning. (播撒激进化文本复数性，使阅读成为受控不稳定性的场域，而非隐藏单一意义的提取。)  
  
### 14. Pharmakon: The Problem of Ambivalent Remedy and Poison  
  
`Pharmakon (药/毒; el: φάρμακον; fr: pharmakon)`  
**Definition:** a term that means both remedy and poison, showing the instability of binary opposition. (一个同时意味着药与毒的术语，显示二元对立的不稳定。)  
**Problem solved:** it exposes cases where a concept cannot be placed cleanly on one side of a hierarchy. (它揭示一个概念无法被干净地放入等级结构某一侧的情形。)  
**Why needed:** philosophical oppositions often depend on terms that both support and disturb them. (哲学对立常依赖既支撑又扰乱这些对立的术语。)  
**How to use:** use it when a supposedly dangerous supplement is also necessary as cure, support, or condition. (当一个所谓危险的补充物同时又是治疗、支撑或条件时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
In Derrida’s reading of Plato, writing is treated as a pharmakon: it is dangerous because it may weaken memory, but useful because it preserves speech. It is both poison and remedy. It cannot be simply condemned or simply celebrated.  
  
This term is useful beyond Plato. Technology can be pharmakon. Law can be pharmakon. Memory can be pharmakon. Platforms, archives, medicine, education, and identity categories can all function as both remedy and poison.  
  
**Typical sentence:** The pharmakon disturbs a hierarchy because it is both what threatens and what supports the system. (Pharmakon 扰乱等级结构，因为它既威胁系统，又支撑系统。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Binary Opposition (二元对立; fr: opposition binaire)** separates terms; **Pharmakon (药/毒; el: φάρμακον)** marks a term that crosses and destabilizes the separation. (二元对立区分术语；pharmakon 标记跨越并动摇这种区分的术语。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** pharmakon becomes a model for reading ambivalent institutions and technologies without reducing them to good or bad. (Pharmakon 成为阅读暧昧制度与技术的模型，使其不被化约为好或坏。)  
  
### 15. Undecidability: The Problem of Necessary Non-Closure  
  
`Undecidability (不可判定性; fr: indécidabilité)`  
**Definition:** a structural condition in which a text, concept, or situation cannot be resolved by applying an existing rule without remainder. (文本、概念或情境无法通过应用既有规则而无剩余地解决的结构状态。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains why decision, interpretation, and judgment cannot be reduced to mechanical rule-application. (它解释为什么决断、解释和判断不能被化约为机械规则应用。)  
**Why needed:** many concepts operate at points where binary categories fail to settle the case. (许多概念在二元分类无法解决案例的位置运作。)  
**How to use:** use it when a decision is required but no rule can fully determine it in advance. (当必须作出决断而没有规则能够预先完全规定它时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Undecidability does not mean indecision or paralysis. It means that a real decision is needed precisely because the rule does not decide by itself. If the rule mechanically determined the outcome, there would be no decision.  
  
This is crucial for law. A judge cannot simply abandon rules. But applying a rule to a singular case requires interpretation. The case both falls under the rule and tests the rule.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Undecidability is not the absence of decision; it is the condition that makes a real decision necessary. (不可判定性不是没有决断，而是使真正决断成为必要的条件。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Indeterminacy (不确定性; en: indeterminacy)** may mean lack of information; **Undecidability (不可判定性; fr: indécidabilité)** means a structural excess that no available rule fully masters. (不确定性可以指信息不足；不可判定性指没有既有规则能够完全掌控的结构性剩余。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** undecidability connects deconstruction to ethics, law, politics, and responsibility. Decision is not less serious because it lacks final foundation; it is more serious. (不可判定性把解构连接到伦理、法律、政治和责任。决断并不因为缺乏最终根据而不严肃；恰恰因此更严肃。)  
  
### 16. Aporia: The Problem of Impossible Passage  
  
`Aporia (难题/无路; el: ἀπορία; fr: aporie)`  
**Definition:** an impasse in which thought must pass but finds no fully available path. (思想必须通过却找不到完全可用路径的困境。)  
**Problem solved:** it names a blockage internal to a concept, system, or demand. (它命名概念、系统或要求内部的阻塞。)  
**Why needed:** ethical, legal, and philosophical problems often require movement through contradictions that cannot be simply solved. (伦理、法律和哲学问题常要求穿过无法简单解决的矛盾。)  
**How to use:** use it when a text confronts an unavoidable but impossible demand: justice, forgiveness, hospitality, gift, decision, responsibility. (当文本面对一种不可避免却又不可能完全实现的要求时，应使用这一概念：正义、宽恕、好客、赠与、决断、责任。)  
  
Aporia is not merely confusion. It is a structured impasse. For Derrida, the most important concepts often contain aporias. Justice must be universal, but every case is singular. Hospitality must welcome the stranger, but unconditional hospitality threatens the household that welcomes. Forgiveness is pure only if it forgives the unforgivable, but that seems impossible.  
  
Aporia marks the point where philosophy cannot proceed by simple concept-application.  
  
**Typical sentence:** An aporia is an impasse where thought must proceed without a guaranteed passage. (难题是思想必须前行却没有保证通道的困境。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Problem (问题; el: πρόβλημα)** may have a solution; **Aporia (难题; el: ἀπορία)** marks a structurally blocked passage. (问题可能有解；难题标记结构性受阻的通道。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** aporia turns deconstruction toward ethics and politics. It shows that responsibility begins where rules fail to guarantee the path. (难题把解构转向伦理和政治，显示责任始于规则无法保证道路之处。)  
  
### 17. Parergon: The Problem of Frame and Work  
  
`Parergon (附属物/框架; el: πάρεργον; fr: parergon)`  
**Definition:** that which appears outside or beside the work but helps constitute the work as work. (看似在作品之外或旁边，却帮助作品作为作品成立的东西。)  
**Problem solved:** it destabilizes the boundary between inside and outside. (它动摇内部与外部之间的边界。)  
**Why needed:** frames, margins, titles, signatures, prefaces, institutions, museums, and genres shape how a work appears. (框架、边缘、标题、签名、序言、制度、博物馆和文类塑造作品如何显现。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing something treated as external support that actually helps define the object. (当分析被视为外部支撑却实际上帮助定义对象的东西时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
In aesthetics, the frame seems outside the painting. But without the frame, display space, museum, label, genre, and institution, the work may not appear as art in the same way. The outside helps constitute the inside.  
  
The parergon is useful for law and philosophy too. Footnotes, prefaces, jurisdiction, institutional setting, citation practices, and procedural forms may seem external to argument or judgment, yet they shape authority and meaning.  
  
**Typical sentence:** The parergon is neither simply inside nor simply outside; it frames the work and thereby helps constitute it. (Parergon 既不只是内部，也不只是外部；它框定作品，并由此帮助构成作品。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Frame (框架; en: frame)** may seem external; **Parergon (附属物/框架; el: πάρεργον)** names the frame’s constitutive role. (框架可能显得外在；parergon 命名框架的构成性作用。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** parergon gives deconstruction a tool for analyzing boundaries: artwork/context, law/procedure, text/margin, argument/apparatus, body/clothing, institution/supplement. (Parergon 为解构提供边界分析工具：作品/语境、法律/程序、文本/边缘、论证/装置、身体/衣着、制度/补充。)  
  
### 18. The Gift: The Problem of Impossible Purity  
  
`Gift (赠与; fr: don)`  
**Definition:** a giving that would have to escape exchange, debt, recognition, reciprocity, and self-credit in order to be pure. (一种若要纯粹就必须逃离交换、债务、承认、互惠和自我功绩的给予。)  
**Problem solved:** it exposes the aporia inside pure generosity. (它揭示纯粹慷慨内部的难题。)  
**Why needed:** many ethical ideals require purity that their own conditions make impossible. (许多伦理理想要求纯粹性，而其自身条件又使这种纯粹性不可能。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing charity, gratitude, debt, recognition, sacrifice, hospitality, or moral credit. (当分析慈善、感激、债务、承认、牺牲、好客或道德功绩时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
For a pure gift, the giver should not expect return. But even recognition as giver may return symbolic credit. If the recipient recognizes the gift as gift, gratitude and debt arise. If the giver recognizes the gift as gift, self-satisfaction may arise. The gift seems possible only by becoming impossible as pure gift.  
  
This does not mean giving never happens. It means pure giving cannot be stabilized as a concept without contradiction.  
  
**Typical sentence:** The gift is possible as practice, but impossible as pure self-present generosity. (赠与作为实践是可能的，但作为纯粹自我在场的慷慨是不可能的。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Exchange (交换; fr: échange)** circulates return; **Gift (赠与; fr: don)** seeks to exceed return but is haunted by it. (交换循环回报；赠与试图超出回报，却被回报所萦绕。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** gift analysis turns deconstruction toward ethics: the highest ethical concepts often function through impossible demands. (赠与分析把解构转向伦理：最高伦理概念常通过不可能的要求运作。)  
  
### 19. Hospitality: The Problem of Conditional and Unconditional Welcome  
  
`Hospitality (好客/接待; la: hospitalitas; fr: hospitalité)`  
**Definition:** the relation of welcoming the stranger, divided between conditional rules and unconditional openness. (接待陌生人的关系，分裂于有条件规则和无条件开放之间。)  
**Problem solved:** it exposes the aporia of welcoming the other. (它揭示接待他者的难题。)  
**Why needed:** hospitality requires a home, boundary, host, and rules, yet unconditional hospitality would suspend mastery over the home. (好客需要家、边界、主人和规则，但无条件好客又会暂停主人对家的控制。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing migration, asylum, borders, guesthood, ethics of the stranger, or political belonging. (当分析移民、庇护、边境、客人身份、陌生人伦理或政治归属时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Conditional hospitality says: welcome, but under rules. Name, passport, visa, invitation, duration, conduct, eligibility. Unconditional hospitality says: welcome the stranger as stranger, before conditions. But without any conditions, hospitality may destroy the very home that hosts.  
  
This is not a simple policy formula. It is an aporia. Political life must use conditions. Ethical responsibility is disturbed by what exceeds conditions.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Hospitality requires conditions to exist, but its ethical force points beyond conditions. (好客需要条件才能存在，但其伦理力量指向条件之外。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Conditional Hospitality (有条件好客; fr: hospitalité conditionnelle)** regulates entry; **Unconditional Hospitality (无条件好客; fr: hospitalité inconditionnelle)** opens to the other before calculation. (有条件好客规制进入；无条件好客在计算之前向他者开放。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** hospitality connects deconstruction to migration, sovereignty, borders, cosmopolitanism, and ethics of alterity. (好客把解构连接到移民、主权、边境、世界主义和他者伦理。)  
  
### 20. Justice and Law: The Problem of Decision under Undecidability  
  
`Justice (正义; la: iustitia; fr: justice)`  
**Definition:** for Derrida, not simply a legal norm, but an incalculable demand for responsibility to the singular other. (对德里达而言，正义不只是法律规范，而是对具体他者的不可计算的责任要求。)  
**Problem solved:** it distinguishes justice from positive law and rule application. (它把正义同实定法和规则应用区分开来。)  
**Why needed:** law is general and calculable; justice addresses singularity that cannot be exhausted by law. (法律是一般的、可计算的；正义面对法律无法穷尽的单一性。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing legal judgment, responsibility, singular cases, undecidability, or the limits of rules. (当分析法律判断、责任、单一案例、不可判定性或规则限度时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
`Law (法律; la: lex; fr: droit/loi)`  
**Definition:** a system of rules, institutions, procedures, rights, and enforceable norms. (由规则、制度、程序、权利和可执行规范组成的系统。)  
**Problem solved:** it gives order, generality, and calculability to social life. (它为社会生活提供秩序、一般性和可计算性。)  
**Why needed:** justice cannot operate publicly without institutional forms, but these forms never exhaust justice. (正义若无制度形式就无法公共地运作，但这些形式从不穷尽正义。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing rule, procedure, enforceability, legal authority, or institutional judgment. (当分析规则、程序、可执行性、法律权威或制度判断时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Derrida’s legal point is subtle. Law is deconstructible because it is historical, textual, interpretable, and revisable. Justice is not deconstructible in the same way because it is the demand that drives deconstruction: the demand to respond to the other beyond settled rules.  
  
This does not mean justice exists as a simple transcendent object. It means justice functions as an impossible demand that prevents law from closing upon itself.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Law is calculable and deconstructible; justice is the incalculable demand that prevents law from becoming final. (法律是可计算且可解构的；正义是阻止法律成为最终者的不可计算要求。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Rule Application (规则应用; en: rule application)** follows a general form; **Justice (正义; fr: justice)** demands responsibility to the singular case. (规则应用遵循一般形式；正义要求对单一案例负责。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** deconstruction enters legal and political theory by showing that judgment must pass through undecidability rather than escape it. (解构通过显示判断必须穿过不可判定性而非逃避它，进入法律与政治理论。)  
  
### 21. The Derridean Reading Method  
  
Derridean reading should not become decorative jargon. It is a disciplined operation. The method can be used in five steps.  
  
**First:** identify the binary hierarchy. (第一，识别二元等级。)  
Examples: speech/writing, presence/absence, nature/culture, literal/metaphorical, original/copy, law/justice, inside/outside, human/animal. (例子：言语/书写、在场/缺席、自然/文化、字面/隐喻、原本/复制、法律/正义、内部/外部、人/动物。)  
  
**Second:** identify the privileged term. (第二，识别被优先化的术语。)  
The privileged term usually claims purity, priority, immediacy, origin, authority, or self-sufficiency. (被优先化术语通常声称纯粹性、优先性、直接性、起源性、权威性或自足性。)  
  
**Third:** identify the subordinated term. (第三，识别被贬低的术语。)  
The subordinated term is often treated as derivative, dangerous, secondary, artificial, excessive, or parasitic. (被贬低术语常被视为派生的、危险的、次要的、人造的、过剩的或寄生的。)  
  
**Fourth:** show dependence. (第四，显示依赖关系。)  
Ask how the privileged term needs the subordinated term in order to function. (追问被优先化术语如何需要被贬低术语才能运作。)  
  
**Fifth:** show instability, not simple reversal. (第五，显示不稳定，而非简单反转。)  
Deconstruction does not merely say writing is better than speech or absence is better than presence. It shows that the hierarchy cannot secure itself. (解构并不只是说书写优于言语，或缺席优于在场。它显示等级结构无法自我保证。)  
  
**Typical sentence:** A Derridean reading does not reverse a hierarchy and stop; it shows why the hierarchy depends on what it subordinates. (德里达式阅读并不只是反转等级后停下；它显示该等级为何依赖其所贬低者。)  
  
### 22. The Tool-Map of Derrida  
  
Use Derridean vocabulary diagnostically. The core question is usually not “what is the hidden meaning?” but “what hierarchy makes this meaning appear stable, and what trace destabilizes it?”  
  
**If the text privileges origin, immediacy, voice, or self-presence**, look for **Metaphysics of Presence (在场形而上学; fr: métaphysique de la présence)**, **Logocentrism (逻各斯中心主义; fr: logocentrisme)**, and **Phonocentrism (语音中心主义; fr: phonocentrisme)**.  
(如果文本优先化起源、直接性、声音或自我在场，应寻找在场形而上学、逻各斯中心主义和语音中心主义问题。)  
  
**If the text treats writing or mediation as secondary**, look for **Writing (书写; fr: écriture)** and **Archi-Writing (原书写; fr: archi-écriture)**.  
(如果文本把书写或中介视为次要，应寻找书写与原书写问题。)  
  
**If the text depends on difference and delayed meaning**, look for **Différance (延异; fr: différance)** and **Trace (痕迹; fr: trace)**.  
(如果文本依赖差异和延迟意义，应寻找延异和痕迹问题。)  
  
**If the text needs an addition it calls secondary**, look for **Supplement (补充; fr: supplément)**.  
(如果文本需要一个它称为次要的添加物，应寻找补充问题。)  
  
**If a sign, rule, signature, or category travels across contexts**, look for **Iterability (可迭代性; fr: itérabilité)**, **Context (语境; fr: contexte)**, and **Signature (签名; fr: signature)**.  
(如果符号、规则、签名或分类跨语境运作，应寻找可迭代性、语境和签名问题。)  
  
**If meaning spreads beyond a single final sense**, look for **Dissemination (播撒; fr: dissémination)**.  
(如果意义扩散而无法回到单一最终意义，应寻找播撒问题。)  
  
**If a term is both remedy and poison**, look for **Pharmakon (药/毒; el: φάρμακον)**.  
(如果一个术语同时是药与毒，应寻找 pharmakon 问题。)  
  
**If a decision is required but no rule fully determines it**, look for **Undecidability (不可判定性; fr: indécidabilité)** and **Aporia (难题; fr: aporie)**.  
(如果必须决断但没有规则能够完全规定，应寻找不可判定性与难题问题。)  
  
**If the boundary between inside and outside matters**, look for **Parergon (附属物/框架; el: πάρεργον)**.  
(如果内部与外部的边界很关键，应寻找 parergon 问题。)  
  
**If the text concerns ethics, law, or politics beyond rules**, look for **Justice (正义; fr: justice)**, **Gift (赠与; fr: don)**, and **Hospitality (好客; fr: hospitalité)**.  
(如果文本涉及超出规则的伦理、法律或政治，应寻找正义、赠与和好客问题。)  
  
### 23. The Genealogical Point of Part 14  
  
Derrida transforms the problem of philosophical language by showing that meaning is never secured by pure presence. Greek philosophy elevated **Logos (逻各斯; el: λόγος)** as speech, reason, and account. Latin metaphysics stabilized meaning through essence, substance, law, and presence. Early modern philosophy centered consciousness and representation. Phenomenology returned to givenness. Heidegger reopened Being and unconcealment. Structuralism showed that meaning depends on systems of difference. Foucault showed that discourse produces truth and subjects through power/knowledge.  
  
Derrida asks what each of these projects must exclude in order to appear stable.  
  
The guiding thesis is:  
  
**Derridean language turns philosophy into the analysis of unstable conditions of meaning: to understand a concept, text, law, or institution is to ask what presence it claims, what hierarchy it builds, what supplement it needs, what trace it carries, and what undecidable decision it tries to conceal.**  
(德里达式语言把哲学转化为对意义不稳定条件的分析：理解一个概念、文本、法律或制度，就是追问它声称何种在场，建立何种等级，需要何种补充，携带何种痕迹，并试图遮蔽何种不可判定的决断。)  
  
This grammar is indispensable for reading metaphysics, law, literature, political theory, theology, gender, colonial discourse, media, archives, digital identity, and institutional authority. It does not abolish truth, law, ethics, or meaning. It prevents them from pretending to be complete, pure, and self-grounded.  
  
The Derridean question remains one of the strongest tools for philosophical reading:  
  
**What must this text subordinate or exclude in order to make its meaning appear present, stable, and authoritative?**  
(这个文本为了使其意义显得在场、稳定且具有权威性，必须贬低或排除什么？)  
  
What supplement does it secretly need in order to appear complete?  
(它为了显得完整，暗中需要什么补充？)  
  
What trace of the excluded term remains inside the privileged term?  
(被排除项的什么痕迹仍然留在被优先化的术语内部？)  
  
Where does the text’s own logic begin to unsettle the hierarchy it tries to maintain?  
(文本自身的逻辑在哪里开始动摇它试图维持的等级结构？)  
  
What decision does the text present as already settled, even though it depends on an undecidable opposition?  
(文本把什么决断呈现为已经解决，尽管它实际上依赖一种不可判定的对立？)  
  
The Derridean question remains one of the strongest tools for philosophical reading:  
(德里达式问题仍然是哲学阅读中最强的工具之一：)  
  
**What must this text subordinate or exclude in order to make its meaning appear present, stable, and authoritative? What supplement does it need, what trace does it carry, and where does its own logic begin to undo the hierarchy it claims to secure?**  
(这个文本为了使其意义显得在场、稳定且具有权威性，必须贬低或排除什么？它需要什么补充，携带什么痕迹，又在何处因自身逻辑而开始瓦解它声称要保证的等级结构？)  
  
## Part 15. Psychoanalysis and Lacan: Unconscious, Desire, Symbolic Order  
  
This chapter explains psychoanalysis as a philosophy of the divided subject. Earlier chapters treated subjectivity through **self-consciousness**, **freedom**, **being-in-the-world**, **discourse**, **power**, and **textual instability**. Psychoanalysis adds a different wound to the modern subject: **the subject is not master in its own house**. (主体并不是自身家中的主人。)  
  
The central question is not simply **what does a person think?** It is: **what speaks, repeats, desires, and suffers in the subject beyond conscious self-knowledge?** (在自觉认识之外，主体之中是什么在说话、重复、欲望和受苦？)  
  
The central vocabulary is **Unconscious**, **Repression**, **Symptom**, **Drive**, **Repetition**, **Transference**, **Desire**, **Lack**, **Fantasy**, **Mirror Stage**, **Imaginary**, **Symbolic**, **Real**, **Other**, **Signifier**, **Barred Subject**, **objet petit a**, **Jouissance**, **Phallus**, **Name-of-the-Father**, and **Four Discourses**. Lacanian psychoanalysis becomes clearer after structural linguistics and analytic language work, because Lacan’s decisive move is to read Freud through Saussure and to treat the unconscious as structured like a language; its core framework includes the three registers, the Other, objet petit a, jouissance, and the phallus as signifier.  
  
The operational function of this chapter is exact: use psychoanalytic vocabulary when the problem is **not what the subject consciously means**, but **what unconscious structure, fantasy, lack, desire, repetition, or symbolic law organizes the subject’s speech and action**. (当问题不是主体自觉地意味着什么，而是什么无意识结构、幻想、缺失、欲望、重复或象征律法组织了主体的言说与行动时，应使用精神分析词汇。)  
  
### 1. The Problem-Situation: The Subject Is Split  
  
Modern philosophy often seeks transparency. Descartes wants certainty in the **Cogito (我思; la: cogito)**. Kant asks for the transcendental conditions of experience. Hegel makes consciousness historical and social. Existentialism makes the subject responsible for its freedom. Foucault analyzes how subjects are produced by discourse and power. Derrida shows that meaning is never fully present.  
  
Psychoanalysis intervenes at another point:  
  
**The subject does not coincide with itself.**  
(主体并不与自身重合。)  
  
A person can speak without knowing what their speech reveals. A person can desire what they consciously reject. A person can repeat what harms them. A person can identify with an image that alienates them. A person can suffer from a symptom that has meaning but not transparent meaning.  
  
This changes the philosophical grammar of subjectivity.  
  
Not: **I think, therefore I am fully present to myself.**  
(不是：我思，所以我完全对自身在场。)  
  
But: **I speak, desire, repeat, and fail in ways that exceed conscious mastery.**  
(而是：我以超出自觉掌控的方式言说、欲望、重复并失败。)  
  
**Typical sentence:** Psychoanalysis treats the subject as divided between conscious self-understanding and unconscious formation. (精神分析把主体理解为分裂于自觉自我理解与无意识形成之间。)  
  
### 2. Psychoanalysis: The Problem of Meaning in Suffering  
  
`Psychoanalysis (精神分析; de: Psychoanalyse; fr: psychanalyse)`  
**Definition:** a theory and clinical practice that interprets symptoms, dreams, desire, speech, and repetition as formations of the unconscious. (一种理论与临床实践，它把症状、梦、欲望、言说和重复解释为无意识的形成物。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains why human suffering often has meaning without being consciously intended. (它解释为什么人的痛苦常常具有意义，却并非由意识有意安排。)  
**Why needed:** the subject’s speech and action are not exhausted by conscious reason, choice, or self-report. (主体的言说和行动不能被自觉理性、选择或自我报告穷尽。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing symptoms, slips, dreams, fantasies, repetitions, desire, trauma, or conflicted selfhood. (当分析症状、口误、梦、幻想、重复、欲望、创伤或冲突性自我时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Psychoanalysis is not simply a psychology of hidden motives. It is a theory of subject-formation. The symptom is not just malfunction. It is a compromise formation. Desire is not just preference. It is structured by lack and fantasy. Speech is not just communication. It is also where the unconscious appears.  
  
This is why psychoanalysis matters for philosophy. It makes the subject opaque, divided, linguistic, historical, embodied, and symptomatic.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Psychoanalysis reads suffering as meaningful, but not as transparently meaningful to the sufferer. (精神分析把痛苦读作有意义的，但这种意义并不对受苦者透明。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Psychology (心理学; el: ψυχή + λόγος)** often studies mental processes empirically; **Psychoanalysis (精神分析; de: Psychoanalyse)** studies unconscious formations through speech, desire, symptom, and transference. (心理学常以经验方式研究心理过程；精神分析通过言说、欲望、症状和移情研究无意识形成物。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** psychoanalysis breaks the sovereignty of the modern subject. After Freud, self-knowledge becomes a problem rather than a given. (精神分析打破现代主体的主权。弗洛伊德之后，自我知识成为问题，而非既定前提。)  
  
### 3. Unconscious: The Problem of Thought beyond Consciousness  
  
`Unconscious (无意识; de: das Unbewusste; fr: inconscient)`  
**Definition:** a structured domain of psychic life that affects speech, desire, symptom, and action without being directly available to consciousness. (一种结构化的心理生活领域，它影响言说、欲望、症状和行动，却不能直接为意识所把握。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains why subjects say, do, desire, and repeat things they do not consciously understand. (它解释为什么主体会说出、做出、欲望和重复自身并不自觉理解的东西。)  
**Why needed:** consciousness cannot explain its own failures, slips, compulsions, and symptomatic formations by itself. (意识无法仅凭自身解释自身的失败、口误、强迫和症状形成。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing hidden structure in speech, fantasy, symptom, dream, repetition, or desire. (当分析言说、幻想、症状、梦、重复或欲望中的隐藏结构时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
The unconscious is not merely a storage room of forgotten memories. For Freud, it is dynamic: repressed material returns in disguised forms. For Lacan, it is structured like a language: it operates through signifiers, substitutions, displacements, and gaps. Lacan’s central move is to read Freud through Saussure and treat the unconscious as structured like a language.  
  
This means unconscious meaning is not private inner substance. It is articulated through speech, slips, repetitions, metaphors, symptoms, and symbolic positions.  
  
**Typical sentence:** The unconscious is not outside language; in Lacan, it is structured through signifiers. (无意识并不在语言之外；在拉康那里，它通过能指被结构化。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Nonconscious (非意识; en: nonconscious)** may mean mental processing outside awareness; **Unconscious (无意识; de: Unbewusste; fr: inconscient)** in psychoanalysis means a dynamic structure of repression, desire, and signification. (非意识可以指意识之外的信息处理；精神分析中的无意识则是压抑、欲望和表意的动态结构。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** the unconscious transforms the philosophical subject. The subject is no longer identical with self-consciousness. (无意识改造哲学主体。主体不再等同于自我意识。)  
  
### 4. Repression: The Problem of Return  
  
`Repression (压抑; de: Verdrängung; fr: refoulement)`  
**Definition:** the psychic process by which unacceptable wishes, representations, or conflicts are excluded from consciousness while continuing to operate unconsciously. (不可接受的愿望、表象或冲突被排除出意识却继续在无意识中运作的心理过程。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains why what is excluded does not disappear but returns in disguised forms. (它解释为什么被排除之物并未消失，而是以伪装形式返回。)  
**Why needed:** subjects often suffer not from simple ignorance, but from what they must not know about their own desire. (主体的痛苦常不来自简单无知，而来自其关于自身欲望所不能知道的东西。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing symptoms, slips, dreams, compulsions, or repeated failures as returns of excluded material. (当把症状、口误、梦、强迫或重复失败分析为被排除材料的返回时，应使用这一概念。)
