Repression is not simple forgetting. Forgotten material may vanish from attention. Repressed material remains active. It returns indirectly: in a symptom, a joke, a dream image, an affective overreaction, a failed action, or a repetitive relational pattern.  
  
This gives psychoanalytic interpretation its logic. The question is not only what is absent. The question is how the absent returns.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Repression excludes a conflict from consciousness, but the excluded conflict returns through symptoms and substitutions. (压抑把冲突排除出意识，但被排除的冲突通过症状和替代返回。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Suppression (抑制; en: suppression)** can be conscious avoidance; **Repression (压抑; de: Verdrängung)** is unconscious exclusion with symptomatic return. (抑制可以是有意识的回避；压抑是带有症状性返回的无意识排除。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** repression connects psychoanalysis with Derrida and Foucault. What is excluded does not vanish; it returns as trace, symptom, discourse, or abnormality. (压抑把精神分析同德里达和福柯连接起来。被排除之物不会消失，而会作为痕迹、症状、话语或异常性返回。)  
  
### 5. Symptom: The Problem of Meaningful Suffering  
  
`Symptom (症状; el: σύμπτωμα; de: Symptom; fr: symptôme)`  
**Definition:** a formation of the unconscious in which conflict, desire, and repression appear as suffering, blockage, bodily disturbance, or repetitive pattern. (一种无意识形成物，其中冲突、欲望和压抑以痛苦、阻滞、身体扰动或重复模式的形式出现。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains suffering as structured rather than merely accidental. (它把痛苦解释为结构化的，而非单纯偶然的。)  
**Why needed:** a symptom can carry unconscious meaning even when it appears irrational or useless. (症状即使显得非理性或无用，也可能携带无意识意义。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing a recurring failure, bodily sign, narrative blockage, compulsive relation, or contradiction that expresses unconscious conflict. (当分析表达无意识冲突的重复失败、身体标记、叙事阻滞、强迫性关系或矛盾时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
The symptom is not just an error to be removed. It is a solution that has become suffering. It allows a conflict to be expressed indirectly. This is why the symptom can be stubborn: it performs a function.  
  
For Lacan, the symptom is also linguistic. It is bound to signifiers, substitutions, and the subject’s relation to the Other. The symptom says something, but not in ordinary propositional form.  
  
**Typical sentence:** A symptom is a message whose meaning is disguised by the very form in which it appears. (症状是一种信息，其意义被其出现形式本身所伪装。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Sign (符号; fr: signe)** points to meaning in a system; **Symptom (症状; fr: symptôme)** is a signifying formation produced by unconscious conflict. (符号在系统中指向意义；症状是由无意识冲突生产的表意形成物。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** symptom-reading becomes a general cultural method. Texts, institutions, ideologies, and social rituals can be read symptomatically when they reveal what they cannot openly say. (症状阅读成为一般文化方法。当文本、制度、意识形态和社会仪式暴露其无法公开言说之物时，就可以被症状性地阅读。)  
  
### 6. Drive: The Problem of Repetition beyond Need  
  
`Drive (驱力; de: Trieb; fr: pulsion)`  
**Definition:** a psychic force that circulates around objects and satisfaction without being reducible to biological need. (一种围绕对象与满足而循环的心理力量，不能被化约为生物需要。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains why human wanting is repetitive, excessive, indirect, and not satisfied by simple need-fulfillment. (它解释为什么人的想要具有重复性、过剩性、间接性，并不能由简单需求满足来解决。)  
**Why needed:** human desire does not operate like hunger alone; it is structured by fantasy, language, prohibition, and partial satisfaction. (人的欲望不像饥饿那样运作；它由幻想、语言、禁令和部分满足结构化。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing repetitive satisfaction, compulsion, bodily fixation, enjoyment, or circular pursuit. (当分析重复性满足、强迫、身体固着、享乐或循环性追求时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Freud’s **Trieb** is often mistranslated as “instinct.” Instinct suggests a natural program with a fixed object. Drive is more unstable. It can displace objects, repeat failure, and find satisfaction in its own circuit.  
  
This distinction matters. The subject may not want the object simply to possess it. The subject may want the repetition, the chase, the loss, the prohibition, the suffering, or the return.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Drive is not satisfied by reaching an object once; it repeats a circuit of partial satisfaction. (驱力并不是通过一次性获得对象而满足；它重复一种部分满足的回路。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Need (需要; fr: besoin)** aims at an object that can satisfy biological lack; **Drive (驱力; fr: pulsion)** circulates around satisfaction in a repetitive structure. (需要指向能够满足生物缺乏的对象；驱力围绕一种重复结构中的满足而循环。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** drive complicates rational agency. The subject is not only a chooser of ends; it is inhabited by repetitive circuits of satisfaction. (驱力使理性行动者概念复杂化。主体不只是目的的选择者，也被重复性的满足回路占据。)  
  
### 7. Repetition: The Problem of Returning to What Harms  
  
`Repetition Compulsion (重复强迫; de: Wiederholungszwang; fr: compulsion de répétition)`  
**Definition:** the tendency to repeat patterns, scenes, failures, or traumatic structures beyond conscious intention and beyond pleasure. (超出意识意图和快乐原则而重复模式、场景、失败或创伤结构的倾向。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains why subjects return to harmful arrangements. (它解释为什么主体会返回伤害自身的配置。)  
**Why needed:** human action cannot be explained only by rational interest or pleasure-seeking. (人的行动不能仅由理性利益或追求快乐来解释。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing recurring relationships, repeated self-sabotage, compulsive narrative loops, or historical return of trauma. (当分析重复性关系、自我破坏、强迫性叙事循环或创伤的历史返回时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Repetition is one of psychoanalysis’s sharpest tools. A person may consciously want change but unconsciously repeat the same structure: choosing the same kind of partner, failing at the same threshold, provoking the same rejection, returning to the same humiliation, reproducing the same institutional scene.  
  
The point is not to moralize repetition. The point is to ask what structure is being repeated and what satisfaction or unresolved conflict is tied to it.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Repetition shows that the subject may be attached not only to pleasure, but to a structure of failure. (重复显示主体可能依附的不只是快乐，也可能是一种失败结构。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Habit (习惯; la: habitus)** can be learned routine; **Repetition Compulsion (重复强迫; de: Wiederholungszwang)** is a symptomatic return of unresolved structure. (习惯可以是习得性常规；重复强迫则是未解决结构的症状性返回。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** repetition links Freud to Nietzsche’s eternal return, Lacan’s signifier-chain, and later cultural theory’s analysis of trauma and ideology. (重复把弗洛伊德同尼采的永恒回归、拉康的能指链以及后来的创伤和意识形态分析连接起来。)  
  
### 8. Transference: The Problem of Repetition in Relation  
  
`Transference (移情; de: Übertragung; fr: transfert)`  
**Definition:** the displacement of earlier relational patterns, affects, and desires onto the analyst or another present figure. (早期关系模式、情感和欲望向分析师或当前他者的转移。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains why the past is not merely remembered but repeated in present relations. (它解释为什么过去不只是被记忆，而是在当前关系中被重复。)  
**Why needed:** psychoanalysis works not only through interpretation, but through the relation in which repetition becomes active. (精神分析不只通过解释运作，也通过使重复变得活跃的关系运作。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing authority, love, rivalry, dependency, projection, pedagogy, therapy, or institutional attachment. (当分析权威、爱、竞争、依赖、投射、教育、治疗或制度依附时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Transference shows that analysis is not neutral observation. The analytic relation becomes a stage on which unconscious patterns appear. The analysand does not simply report desire; desire is enacted in the relation.  
  
This concept travels beyond clinic. Teacher-student relations, political charisma, religious authority, fandom, mentorship, and institutional loyalty can all involve transferential structures.  
  
Lacanian concepts such as transference have also been applied to creative-writing pedagogy and supervision, where authority, symbolic position, and identification structure the writing relation.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Transference is the repetition of earlier desire and relation in a present scene. (移情是早期欲望与关系在当前场景中的重复。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Projection (投射; de: Projektion)** attributes inner content to another; **Transference (移情; de: Übertragung)** repeats relational structure with another. (投射把内部内容归给他者；移情则同他者重复一种关系结构。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** transference makes knowledge relational. Truth in analysis emerges through the structure of relation, not detached observation. (移情使知识具有关系性。分析中的真理通过关系结构出现，而不是通过脱离式观察出现。)  
  
### 9. Lacan’s Return to Freud: The Problem of Language  
  
`Return to Freud (回到弗洛伊德; fr: retour à Freud)`  
**Definition:** Lacan’s project of rereading Freud through linguistics, structuralism, philosophy, and clinical practice. (拉康通过语言学、结构主义、哲学和临床实践重新阅读弗洛伊德的工程。)  
**Problem solved:** it resists reducing Freud to ego psychology, adaptation, or ordinary therapeutic normalization. (它反抗把弗洛伊德化约为自我心理学、适应或普通治疗性正常化。)  
**Why needed:** Freud’s discovery of the unconscious requires a theory of speech, signifier, desire, and symbolic structure. (弗洛伊德对无意识的发现需要一种关于言说、能指、欲望和象征结构的理论。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing Lacan’s claim that psychoanalysis concerns speech and language before it concerns ego-strength or adaptation. (当分析拉康关于精神分析首先关涉言说和语言，而非自我强度或适应的主张时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Lacan is not simply Freud with French terminology. His key move is structural. He treats the unconscious as articulated through language. This is why **Signifier (能指; fr: signifiant)** becomes central. The subject is not the source of language; the subject is produced in and by the signifying order.  
  
Lacan becomes easier to read after Saussure precisely because his theory becomes intelligible only once structural linguistics is in place. The **Mirror Stage**, the **Rome Discourse**, **The Instance of the Letter**, and **The Subversion of the Subject** provide a conceptual route into Lacan.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Lacan returns to Freud by showing that unconscious formations are structured through signifiers. (拉康通过显示无意识形成物由能指结构化而回到弗洛伊德。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Ego Psychology (自我心理学; en: ego psychology)** strengthens adaptation; **Lacanian Psychoanalysis (拉康派精神分析; fr: psychanalyse lacanienne)** analyzes the divided subject of language and desire. (自我心理学强化适应；拉康派精神分析分析语言与欲望中的分裂主体。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** psychoanalysis becomes linguistic and structural. The unconscious is no longer only depth; it is also a surface of signifiers. (精神分析变得语言化和结构化。无意识不再只是深处，也是一种能指表面。)  
  
### 10. Mirror Stage: The Problem of Ego as Misrecognition  
  
`Mirror Stage (镜像阶段; fr: stade du miroir)`  
**Definition:** Lacan’s account of the infant’s identification with an external image of bodily unity, producing the ego through misrecognition. (拉康关于婴儿认同外部身体统一形象的说明；自我由此通过误认而产生。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains the ego not as original self-presence, but as an alienating identification with an image. (它把自我解释为对形象的异化性认同，而非原初自我在场。)  
**Why needed:** the subject’s sense of unity is formed from outside and is therefore unstable. (主体的统一感由外部形成，因此是不稳定的。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing self-image, rivalry, narcissism, identification, bodily unity, or alienated selfhood. (当分析自我形象、竞争、自恋、认同、身体统一或异化自我时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
The mirror stage is not simply about a literal mirror. It names a structure. The child identifies with an image of unity that exceeds its fragmented bodily experience. The ego is born through an external image that the subject takes as itself.  
  
This has strong philosophical consequences. The ego is not the foundation of truth. It is an imaginary construction. Selfhood begins with misrecognition.  
  
The mirror stage is the conceptual entry to Lacan, and contemporary writers have used it to design misrecognition, self-image, and narrative form.  
  
**Typical sentence:** The mirror stage produces the ego as an identification with an external image of unity. (镜像阶段把自我生产为对外部统一形象的认同。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Self-Knowledge (自我知识; en: self-knowledge)** suggests transparent relation to oneself; **Misrecognition (误认; fr: méconnaissance)** names the false recognition through which the ego is formed. (自我知识暗示同自身的透明关系；误认命名自我借以形成的错误承认。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** the ego becomes suspect. It is not the stable core of subjectivity, but an image-formation. (自我变得可疑。它不是主体性的稳定核心，而是形象形成物。)  
  
### 11. Imaginary: The Problem of Image and Coherence  
  
`Imaginary (想象界; fr: l’Imaginaire)`  
**Definition:** the register of image, identification, rivalry, coherence, and ego-formation. (形象、认同、竞争、连贯性和自我形成的界域。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains how subjects experience themselves and others through images of unity and likeness. (它解释主体如何通过统一和相似的形象经验自身与他者。)  
**Why needed:** selfhood is mediated by images before it is fully articulated in symbolic language. (自我性在完全进入象征语言之前已由形象中介。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing narcissism, rivalry, doubles, ideal images, fantasy coherence, or visual identity. (当分析自恋、竞争、替身、理想形象、幻想性连贯或视觉身份时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
The Imaginary is not simply imagination. It is a register of relation. The ego forms through images. The other appears as rival, double, mirror, ideal, or threat. The Imaginary gives coherence, but that coherence is unstable and alienating.  
  
This is useful for reading literature and social life. Characters often defend an image of themselves. Institutions often produce ideal images. Social media intensifies imaginary identification: profile, image, comparison, visibility, envy, rivalry.  
  
**Typical sentence:** The Imaginary gives the subject an image of unity, but that unity is alienating because it comes from outside. (想象界给予主体统一形象，但这种统一是异化性的，因为它来自外部。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Imaginary (想象界; fr: Imaginaire)** differs from **Imagination (想象; la: imaginatio)**. Imagination is a mental faculty; the Imaginary is a structural register of image-identification. (想象是心理能力；想象界是形象认同的结构性界域。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** the image becomes formative, not decorative. Subjectivity begins not in pure thought, but in alienating identification. (形象成为形成性的，而非装饰性的。主体性不是始于纯思维，而是始于异化性认同。)  
  
### 12. Symbolic: The Problem of Law, Language, and Position  
  
`Symbolic (象征界; fr: le Symbolique)`  
**Definition:** the register of language, law, kinship, social structure, signifiers, and symbolic positions. (语言、律法、亲属关系、社会结构、能指和象征位置的界域。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains how subjects are inserted into language and social order. (它解释主体如何被插入语言与社会秩序。)  
**Why needed:** the subject does not create meaning from nothing; it is positioned within an already existing symbolic order. (主体并非从无中创造意义；它被定位于一个已经存在的象征秩序中。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing law, names, kinship, social roles, grammar, authority, prohibition, or subject-position. (当分析律法、名称、亲属、社会角色、语法、权威、禁令或主体位置时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
The Symbolic is the order of signifiers. It is not merely symbolism. It is the structure into which the subject is born: names, prohibitions, family positions, language, institutions, legal categories, gender terms, and social address.  
  
The subject becomes intelligible only by taking a place in the Symbolic. But this insertion also divides the subject. To speak, one must use signifiers that precede oneself. The subject appears in language, but never fully owns language.  
  
The Lacanian subject is constituted by its place in the symbolic order, which connects subject formation with rule-governed structures in language.  
  
**Typical sentence:** The Symbolic is the order of language and law that gives the subject a place by dividing it. (象征界是语言与律法的秩序，它通过分裂主体而给予主体位置。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Symbol (象征/符号; el: σύμβολον)** can mean a sign standing for something; **Symbolic (象征界; fr: Symbolique)** names the structural order of signifiers, law, and social positions. (象征/符号可以指代表某物的标记；象征界命名能指、律法和社会位置的结构性秩序。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** subjectivity becomes linguistic and institutional. The subject is produced by taking a place in language. (主体性变得语言化和制度化。主体通过在语言中占据位置而被生产。)  
  
### 13. Real: The Problem of What Resists Symbolization  
  
`Real (实在界; fr: le Réel)`  
**Definition:** the register of what resists symbolization, cannot be fully integrated into language, and returns as rupture, trauma, impossibility, or excess. (抵抗符号化、无法被完全整合进语言，并以断裂、创伤、不可能或过剩形式返回的界域。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains why symbolic systems fail, why trauma resists narration, and why desire is never fully satisfied. (它解释为什么象征系统会失败，为什么创伤抵抗叙述，为什么欲望从不被完全满足。)  
**Why needed:** not everything can be made meaningful within the Symbolic. (并非一切都能在象征界中成为有意义之物。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing trauma, breakdown, impossibility, bodily excess, unsayability, or points where language fails. (当分析创伤、崩溃、不可能性、身体过剩、不可言说性或语言失败之处时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
The Real is not ordinary reality. Ordinary reality is already structured by the Imaginary and Symbolic. The Real is what does not fit. It is encountered as impossibility, shock, rupture, or traumatic return.  
  
This makes the Real very different from empirical fact. A fact can be stated. The Real is what disrupts statement itself.  
  
**Typical sentence:** The Real is not reality as object, but what resists being absorbed into the symbolic order. (实在界不是作为对象的现实，而是抵抗被吸收到象征秩序中的东西。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Reality (现实; fr: réalité)** is the world as symbolically and imaginatively organized; **Real (实在界; fr: Réel)** is what resists that organization. (现实是由象征与想象组织起来的世界；实在界是抵抗这种组织的东西。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** the Real gives psychoanalysis a theory of failure. Meaning is powerful, but never complete. (实在界给予精神分析一种失败理论。意义很有力量，但从不完整。)  
  
### 14. Other: The Problem of Language and Desire from Elsewhere  
  
`Other (大他者; fr: grand Autre)`  
**Definition:** the symbolic locus of language, law, recognition, address, and desire. (语言、律法、承认、召唤和欲望的象征位置。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains why the subject’s desire and speech are mediated by something beyond the ego. (它解释为什么主体的欲望和言说由超出自我的东西中介。)  
**Why needed:** the subject speaks in a language that comes from the Other and seeks recognition from the Other. (主体在来自大他者的语言中说话，并寻求来自大他者的承认。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing authority, law, symbolic address, recognition, demand, desire, or institutional speech. (当分析权威、律法、象征召唤、承认、要求、欲望或制度性言说时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
**Usage layers:**  
1. **Phenomenological / existential use (现象学/存在主义用法):** **the Other** names another subject whose presence interrupts self-enclosure, exposes the self, or makes selfhood social and vulnerable. (在现象学和存在主义中，他者指打断自我封闭、暴露自我并使自我具有社会性和脆弱性的另一个主体。)  
  
2. **Lacanian use (拉康式用法):** **the Other** names the field of language, law, symbolic order, and desire from which the subject receives its position and speech. (在拉康那里，大他者指语言、律法、象征秩序和欲望的场域，主体从中获得位置和言说。)  
  
3. **Feminist / postcolonial transferable use (女性主义/后殖民泛用法):** **Other** and **Othering** describe how dominant identities produce excluded, feminized, racialized, colonized, or abnormalized figures as their opposite. (在女性主义和后殖民理论中，他者与他者化指支配性身份如何生产被排除、女性化、种族化、殖民化或异常化的形象作为自身对立面。)  
  
**Transfer rule:** before using **Other**, ask whether the issue is another consciousness, symbolic authority, constitutive exclusion, colonial identity, gendered hierarchy, or social intelligibility. (转用规则：使用 Other 之前，应先判断问题是另一个意识、象征权威、构成性排除、殖民身份、性别等级，还是社会可理解性。)  
  
**Misuse warning:** **Other** is not simply “someone different.” It names a structural relation of selfhood, language, or exclusion. (Other 不只是“不同的人”，而是自我、语言或排除的结构性关系。)  
  
The Other is not simply another person. A parent can occupy the place of the Other. So can law, language, God, institution, state, school, court, clinic, archive, or social order. The Other is the place from which the subject receives signifiers and to which the subject addresses speech.  
  
This is why the subject’s question is often:  
  
**What does the Other want from me?**  
(大他者想从我这里得到什么？)  
  
Desire is shaped by this question.  
  
**Typical sentence:** The subject desires and speaks in relation to the Other, the symbolic place from which recognition and law arrive. (主体在同大他者的关系中欲望和言说；大他者是承认与律法到来的象征位置。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Other Person (他人; fr: autre)** is another empirical person; **Other (大他者; fr: grand Autre)** is the symbolic locus of language, law, and recognition. (他人是经验中的另一个人；大他者是语言、律法与承认的象征位置。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** the Other connects Lacan to Hegelian recognition, structuralism, theology, law, and Foucaultian institutions. (大他者把拉康连接到黑格尔式承认、结构主义、神学、法律和福柯式制度。)  
  
### 15. Signifier: The Problem of the Subject in Language  
  
`Signifier (能指; fr: signifiant)`  
**Definition:** the differential element of language that represents the subject for another signifier. (语言中的差异性元素，它为另一个能指代表主体。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains how the subject appears only through language that also displaces it. (它解释主体如何只通过同时置换主体的语言而出现。)  
**Why needed:** psychoanalysis requires a theory of how speech reveals more than conscious meaning. (精神分析需要一种理论来说明言说如何揭示超出自觉意义的东西。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing slips, names, repeated words, symbolic positions, unconscious chains, or desire structured by language. (当分析口误、名字、重复词、象征位置、无意识链条或由语言结构化的欲望时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
In Saussure, signifier and signified form the sign. Lacan radicalizes the signifier. The signifier does not merely express a concept. It structures the subject. A name, insult, diagnosis, kinship term, gender term, legal status, or institutional label can organize desire and identity.  
  
The subject is caught in signifiers before it can master them. It is named before it names itself. It is spoken before it speaks.  
  
**Typical sentence:** The signifier does not simply communicate meaning; it positions and divides the subject. (能指并不只是传达意义；它定位并分裂主体。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Word (词; en: word)** is a linguistic unit; **Signifier (能指; fr: signifiant)** is a differential element that operates within a symbolic chain. (词是语言单位；能指是在象征链中运作的差异性元素。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** language ceases to be a tool possessed by the subject. It becomes the structure through which the subject is produced. (语言不再是主体拥有的工具，而成为主体借以被生产的结构。)  
  
### 16. Barred Subject: The Problem of Division  
  
`Barred Subject (被划杠主体/分裂主体; fr: sujet barré; notation: $$\bar S$$)`  
**Definition:** the subject divided by language, lack, and the unconscious. (被语言、缺失和无意识分裂的主体。)  
**Problem solved:** it rejects the idea of a self-identical, transparent subject. (它拒绝自我同一且透明的主体观。)  
**Why needed:** the subject can appear in language only by being represented by signifiers that never fully capture it. (主体只能通过能指在语言中出现，而能指从不完全捕获主体。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing self-division, failed self-presence, contradictory desire, or speech that exceeds intention. (当分析自我分裂、自我在场失败、矛盾欲望或超出意图的言说时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
The barred subject is not a sad psychological condition. It is the structure of subjectivity. To enter language is to lose immediate self-presence. The subject is represented by signifiers, but no signifier fully says what the subject is.  
  
This makes the subject permanently split: between what it says and what it means, between demand and desire, between image and law, between conscious intention and unconscious formation.  
  
**Typical sentence:** The barred subject is the subject that appears in language only as divided by language. (被划杠主体是只作为被语言分裂者而在语言中出现的主体。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Ego (自我; la: ego; fr: moi)** is an imaginary formation of coherence; **Subject (主体; fr: sujet)** in Lacan is divided by the signifier. (自我是想象性的连贯形成物；拉康的主体则被能指分裂。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** the subject becomes a gap in the signifying chain, not a sovereign origin. (主体成为能指链中的裂隙，而非主权式起源。)  
  
### 17. Desire: The Problem of Wanting beyond Need  
  
`Desire (欲望; fr: désir)`  
**Definition:** a structured wanting that emerges from lack and is mediated by the Other, language, and fantasy. (一种由缺失产生，并由大他者、语言和幻想中介的结构化想要。)  
**Problem solved:** it distinguishes human desire from biological need and explicit demand. (它把人的欲望同生物需要和明确要求区分开来。)  
**Why needed:** subjects often do not want only the object they say they want; they want recognition, lack, fantasy, and the desire of the Other. (主体常常不只是想要其声称想要的对象；主体想要承认、缺失、幻想以及大他者的欲望。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing why obtaining an object does not end wanting. (当分析为什么获得对象并不会终止想要时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
**Usage layers:**  
1. **Ordinary-psychological use (普通心理用法):** **desire** may mean wanting, preference, appetite, wish, or attraction. This is not yet the technical psychoanalytic sense. (普通心理用法中，desire 可指想要、偏好、欲求、愿望或吸引；这还不是精神分析的技术义。)  
  
2. **Psychoanalytic / Lacanian use (精神分析/拉康式用法):** desire is not simply need or demand. It is structured by lack, language, the Other, fantasy, and the symbolic order. (在精神分析尤其拉康那里，欲望不只是需要或要求，而是由缺失、语言、大他者、幻想和象征秩序结构化。)  
  
3. **Contemporary transferable use (当代理论泛用法):** in feminism, queer theory, postcolonial theory, media studies, and political theory, desire may name socially organized attachment, aspiration, fantasy, normativity, or investment in identity and power. (在女性主义、酷儿理论、后殖民理论、媒介研究和政治理论中，欲望可指被社会组织起来的依附、渴望、幻想、规范性或对身份与权力的投注。)  
  
**Transfer rule:** use **desire** technically when wanting is mediated by lack, language, fantasy, social norm, or symbolic structure. Do not use it merely as a synonym for preference. (转用规则：当“想要”受到缺失、语言、幻想、社会规范或象征结构中介时，才技术性地使用 desire。不要把它仅仅当作 preference 的同义词。)  
  
**Misuse warning:** desire is not reducible to biological need or conscious intention. (Desire 不能化约为生物需要或清醒意图。)  
  
Lacan’s formula is often stated as: **desire is the desire of the Other**. (欲望是大他者的欲望。) This means at least two things. The subject desires what the Other desires. The subject also desires to be desired by the Other.  
  
Desire therefore cannot be reduced to object acquisition. The object is often a support for a deeper structure: recognition, lack, prohibition, fantasy, or symbolic position.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Desire does not simply seek an object; it seeks its place in the desire of the Other. (欲望并不只是寻求对象；它寻求自身在大他者欲望中的位置。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Need (需要; fr: besoin)** can be satisfied by an object; **Desire (欲望; fr: désir)** persists beyond satisfaction because it is structured by lack. (需要可以由对象满足；欲望因由缺失结构化而在满足之后继续存在。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** desire becomes structural rather than psychological preference. The subject wants through language, law, and the Other. (欲望成为结构性的，而非心理偏好。主体通过语言、律法和大他者而欲望。)  
  
### 18. Lack: The Problem of Constitutive Absence  
  
`Lack (缺失; fr: manque)`  
**Definition:** the constitutive absence around which desire is organized. (欲望围绕其被组织的构成性缺席。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains why desire persists and why no object fully satisfies it. (它解释为什么欲望持续存在，以及为什么没有对象能够完全满足它。)  
**Why needed:** the subject is not a complete being that occasionally wants; the subject is structured by lack. (主体不是偶尔想要的完整存在者；主体由缺失结构化。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing incompletion, longing, substitution, fantasy, or the failure of satisfaction. (当分析不完整、渴望、替代、幻想或满足失败时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Lack is not merely empirical deprivation. It is not only “not having something.” It is the structural condition of desire. The subject seeks objects, but the object never fills the lack because the lack belongs to subjectivity itself.  
  
This is why consumer desire, romantic obsession, ambition, symbolic recognition, and ideological attachment can be read psychoanalytically. The object matters, but it is not the whole matter.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Lack is not a missing object; it is the structural incompletion that makes desire possible. (缺失不是一个缺少的对象，而是使欲望成为可能的结构性不完整。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Absence (缺席; fr: absence)** means something is not present; **Lack (缺失; fr: manque)** is the constitutive absence that structures desire. (缺席意味着某物不在场；缺失是结构欲望的构成性缺席。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** lack connects Lacan to Plato’s eros, Hegelian negativity, existential incompletion, and Derridean absence, but gives it a specifically psychoanalytic structure. (缺失把拉康连接到柏拉图的爱欲、黑格尔式否定性、存在主义不完整性和德里达式缺席，但赋予其精神分析结构。)  
  
### 19. objet petit a: The Problem of the Cause of Desire  
  
`objet petit a (小客体 a; fr: objet petit a)`  
**Definition:** the object-cause of desire, not the object that satisfies desire but the elusive remainder that sets desire in motion. (欲望的对象—原因；它不是满足欲望的对象，而是使欲望运动起来的难以捕获的剩余物。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains why desire attaches to objects that never fully satisfy. (它解释为什么欲望会依附于永不完全满足它的对象。)  
**Why needed:** desire needs a lure, but the lure is not the final answer to desire. (欲望需要诱因，但诱因并不是欲望的最终答案。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing the object, detail, voice, gaze, body-part, fantasy element, or unattainable remainder that organizes wanting. (当分析组织想要的对象、细节、声音、凝视、身体部分、幻想元素或不可获得剩余时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
**objet petit a** should not be translated too quickly. It is not simply “object of desire.” It is the object-cause of desire. The subject does not desire because the object is inherently satisfying. The object becomes charged because it stands in for lack.  
  
In literature, this may be a voice, glance, letter, scar, room, absent person, gesture, lost object, or impossible promise. In politics, it may be nation, purity, security, greatness, recognition, or revenge. In consumer culture, it may be the aura attached to a commodity.  
  
**Objet petit a** is one of the Lacanian concepts most portable into writing practice because it helps specify the lure that keeps a story moving.  
  
**Typical sentence:** objet petit a is not what desire wants to possess, but what causes desire to keep moving. (小客体 a 不是欲望想要占有的东西，而是使欲望持续运动的原因。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Desired Object (欲望对象; en: desired object)** is what the subject thinks it wants; **objet petit a (小客体 a; fr: objet petit a)** is the cause that organizes wanting beyond that object. (欲望对象是主体以为自己想要的东西；小客体 a 是在该对象之外组织想要的原因。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** desire becomes non-teleological. It is not a straight path toward satisfaction, but a circuit around a lost or impossible object-cause. (欲望变得非目的论。它不是通向满足的直线路径，而是围绕失落或不可能的对象—原因的回路。)  
  
### 20. Fantasy: The Problem of Desire’s Scenario  
  
`Fantasy (幻想; de: Phantasie; fr: fantasme)`  
**Definition:** the unconscious scenario that stages the subject’s relation to desire, the Other, and objet petit a. (一种无意识场景，它安排主体同欲望、大他者和小客体 a 的关系。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains how desire is organized into repeatable scenes and positions. (它解释欲望如何被组织成可重复场景和位置。)  
**Why needed:** subjects do not desire in a vacuum; they desire through scenes that give desire form. (主体并不在真空中欲望；主体通过赋予欲望形式的场景而欲望。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing recurring scenarios of rescue, humiliation, mastery, abandonment, seduction, sacrifice, revenge, or recognition. (当分析救赎、羞辱、掌控、遗弃、诱惑、牺牲、复仇或承认的重复场景时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Fantasy is not mere daydreaming. It is a structure. It tells the subject where it stands in relation to the Other’s desire. It organizes what counts as desirable, threatening, forbidden, humiliating, or fulfilling.  
  
Fantasy is therefore a key tool for reading ideology. Ideology does not work only by false propositions. It works by fantasy-scenes: threatened nation, stolen enjoyment, pure community, corrupt enemy, heroic sacrifice, innocent victim, restored wholeness.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Fantasy is the scene that teaches the subject how to desire. (幻想是教会主体如何欲望的场景。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Imagination (想象; la: imaginatio)** can produce images freely; **Fantasy (幻想; fr: fantasme)** structures the subject’s desire and relation to the Other. (想象可以自由地产生图像；幻想则结构主体的欲望及其同大他者的关系。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** fantasy connects psychoanalysis to ideology critique, literary theory, political theology, and media analysis. (幻想把精神分析连接到意识形态批判、文学理论、政治神学和媒介分析。)  
  
### 21. Jouissance: The Problem of Enjoyment beyond Pleasure  
  
`Jouissance (享乐; fr: jouissance)`  
**Definition:** excessive enjoyment that goes beyond pleasure, often involving pain, compulsion, transgression, or unbearable satisfaction. (一种超出快乐的过剩享乐，常涉及痛苦、强迫、越界或难以承受的满足。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains why subjects remain attached to suffering or destructive satisfaction. (它解释为什么主体会依附于痛苦或破坏性满足。)  
**Why needed:** pleasure alone cannot explain repetition, addiction, ideological passion, or attachment to symptom. (单靠快乐无法解释重复、成瘾、意识形态激情或对症状的依附。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing painful enjoyment, compulsive repetition, transgressive satisfaction, or ideological enjoyment. (当分析痛苦的享乐、强迫性重复、越界性满足或意识形态享乐时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Jouissance is difficult because it is not ordinary pleasure. Pleasure seeks balance. Jouissance exceeds balance. It can be too much. A subject may suffer from what it enjoys, and enjoy what makes it suffer.  
  
This is indispensable for political and cultural analysis. Hatred can contain jouissance. Moral outrage can contain jouissance. Victimhood, purity, cruelty, self-sacrifice, and humiliation can become libidinally charged.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Jouissance names the enjoyment that persists where pleasure should have stopped. (享乐命名那种在快乐本应停止之处仍持续存在的满足。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Pleasure (快乐; de: Lust; fr: plaisir)** tends toward satisfaction and reduction of tension; **Jouissance (享乐; fr: jouissance)** exceeds pleasure and may become painful. (快乐趋向满足和张力降低；享乐超出快乐，并可能变得痛苦。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** enjoyment becomes political. Subjects are not attached to ideology only because they believe it, but because they enjoy through it. (享乐变得政治化。主体依附意识形态，不只是因为相信它，也因为通过它享乐。)  
  
### 22. Phallus: The Problem of the Signifier of Lack  
  
`Phallus (菲勒斯/阳具能指; fr: phallus)`  
**Definition:** in Lacan, not the biological penis, but the signifier of desire, lack, and symbolic position. (在拉康那里，它不是生物学阴茎，而是欲望、缺失和象征位置的能指。)  
**Problem solved:** it separates psychoanalytic sexual difference from simple anatomy. (它把精神分析中的性差异同简单解剖学区分开来。)  
**Why needed:** symbolic power and desire are organized by signifiers, not merely by biological organs. (象征权力和欲望由能指组织，而不只是由生物器官组织。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing symbolic authority, desire, lack, gendered position, or the fantasy of possessing what completes the Other. (当分析象征权威、欲望、缺失、性别化位置或拥有能使大他者完整之物的幻想时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
The phallus is often misunderstood. It is not a celebration of male anatomy. It is a signifier. It names the place of lack and symbolic value around which desire is organized. No one simply “has” the phallus in a complete way. The phallus marks the fantasy of completion and the impossibility of completion.  
  
This concept is controversial and must be used carefully, especially in feminist and queer theory. Its value lies in analyzing symbolic structures of gendered power, not in naturalizing them.  
  
**Typical sentence:** The phallus is not an organ but a signifier of lack and symbolic desire. (菲勒斯不是器官，而是缺失与象征欲望的能指。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Penis (阴茎; la: penis)** is an anatomical organ; **Phallus (菲勒斯; fr: phallus)** is a symbolic signifier. (阴茎是解剖器官；菲勒斯是象征性能指。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** sexual difference becomes symbolic rather than merely biological. This opens psychoanalysis to both feminist critique and feminist appropriation. (性差异变得象征化，而非仅仅生物化。这使精神分析同时面对女性主义批判和女性主义改造。)  
  
### 23. Name-of-the-Father: The Problem of Symbolic Law  
  
`Name-of-the-Father (父名; fr: Nom-du-Père)`  
**Definition:** the signifier of symbolic law that introduces prohibition, separation, and the subject’s entry into the Symbolic order. (引入禁令、分离和主体进入象征秩序的象征律法能指。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains how desire is structured by prohibition and symbolic mediation. (它解释欲望如何由禁令和象征中介结构化。)  
**Why needed:** the subject must be separated from imaginary fusion in order to enter language, law, and social relation. (主体必须脱离想象性融合，才能进入语言、律法和社会关系。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing symbolic authority, prohibition, kinship structure, law, psychosis, or paternal metaphor. (当分析象征权威、禁令、亲属结构、法律、精神病或父性隐喻时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
The Name-of-the-Father is not simply the empirical father. It is a symbolic function. It represents law, prohibition, and separation. The child is not simply in a dyadic relation with the mother or caregiver; the symbolic third interrupts and structures desire.  
  
This concept is central in Lacan’s theory of psychosis, where the foreclosure of the Name-of-the-Father has major structural consequences.  
  
**Typical sentence:** The Name-of-the-Father is the symbolic function that introduces law and separates the subject from imaginary fusion. (父名是引入律法并使主体脱离想象性融合的象征功能。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Father (父亲; la: pater; fr: père)** is an empirical person; **Name-of-the-Father (父名; fr: Nom-du-Père)** is a symbolic function of law and prohibition. (父亲是经验人物；父名是律法与禁令的象征功能。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** law becomes psychic and linguistic before it is merely juridical. The subject enters law through signifiers. (律法在成为单纯法权之物之前，已经是心理和语言性的。主体通过能指进入律法。)  
  
### 24. Split between Enunciation and Enunciated: The Problem of Saying More than Said  
  
`Enunciation (言说行为; fr: énonciation)`  
**Definition:** the act, position, or scene from which something is said. (某物被说出的行为、位置或场景。)  
**Problem solved:** it reveals what the subject performs in speaking. (它揭示主体在言说中执行了什么。)  
**Why needed:** what a subject says may differ from what the subject does by saying it. (主体所说的内容可能不同于主体通过说它所做的事情。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing tone, position, contradiction, denial, irony, confession, or performative self-exposure. (当分析语气、位置、矛盾、否认、讽刺、忏悔或表演性自我暴露时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
`Enunciated (所言内容; fr: énoncé)`  
**Definition:** the stated content of speech. (言说的被陈述内容。)  
**Problem solved:** it distinguishes what is said from the speaking position that produces it. (它把所说内容同生产它的言说位置区分开来。)  
**Why needed:** unconscious meaning often appears in the gap between statement and act of speaking. (无意识意义常出现在陈述内容与言说行为之间的裂缝中。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing mismatch between declared content and subjective position. (当分析被声明内容与主体位置之间的不一致时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
A person says: “I am not angry.” The enunciated content denies anger. The enunciation may perform anger through tone, insistence, timing, or repetition. Psychoanalysis listens to this gap.  
  
This distinction is also useful for literary and legal reading. A narrator may claim neutrality while performing obsession. A law may claim equality while speaking from a hierarchy. A confession may state guilt while staging innocence.  
  
The split between **enunciation** and **the enunciated** is one of the most portable Lacanian tools for writing and criticism, because it clarifies why narrators or characters say one thing while performing another.  
  
**Typical sentence:** The unconscious often appears not in what is said, but in the gap between what is said and the position from which it is said. (无意识常不出现在所说内容中，而出现在所说内容与说话位置之间的裂缝中。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Statement Content (陈述内容; fr: énoncé)** is what is said; **Enunciation (言说行为; fr: énonciation)** is the act and position of saying. (陈述内容是所说之物；言说行为是说的行动与位置。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** speech becomes divided. Language no longer transparently expresses intention; it stages the subject’s split. (言说变得分裂。语言不再透明表达意图，而是上演主体的分裂。)  
  
### 25. The Four Discourses: The Problem of Social Bond  
  
`Four Discourses (四种话语; fr: quatre discours)`  
**Definition:** Lacan’s formal model of social bonds structured by positions of agent, Other, truth, and product. (拉康关于社会纽带的形式模型，由行动者、大他者、真理和产物的位置结构化。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains how speech organizes authority, knowledge, desire, and social relation. (它解释言说如何组织权威、知识、欲望和社会关系。)  
**Why needed:** discourse is not just content; it is a structure of positions that produces effects. (话语不只是内容，而是生产效果的位置结构。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing authority, teaching, bureaucracy, expertise, capitalism, analysis, or ideological speech. (当分析权威、教学、官僚制、专业知识、资本主义、分析或意识形态言说时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Lacan’s four classical discourses are:  
  
**Master’s Discourse (主人话语; fr: discours du maître)** organizes command and authority. (组织命令与权威。)  
  
**University Discourse (大学话语; fr: discours universitaire)** organizes knowledge as institutional authority. (把知识组织为制度权威。)  
  
**Hysteric’s Discourse (癔症者话语; fr: discours de l’hystérique)** questions the master and exposes lack. (质问主人并暴露缺失。)  
  
**Analyst’s Discourse (分析家话语; fr: discours de l’analyste)** positions the object-cause of desire so that the subject’s truth may emerge. (把欲望的对象—原因置于某种位置，使主体真理得以出现。)  
  
Later, Lacan also develops the **Discourse of the Capitalist (资本主义话语; fr: discours du capitaliste)**, often used to analyze accelerated consumption and endless circulation of desire.  
  
**Typical sentence:** A discourse is not a theme but a structure of positions that organizes who speaks, what counts as knowledge, and what kind of subject is produced. (话语不是主题，而是一种位置结构，它组织谁说话、什么算作知识以及生产什么样的主体。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Discourse (话语; fr: discours)** in Foucault names historical fields of sayability and knowledge; **Discourse (话语; fr: discours)** in Lacan names a formal structure of social bond. (福柯的话语命名可说性与知识的历史场域；拉康的话语命名社会纽带的形式结构。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** Lacanian discourse theory connects psychoanalysis to politics, pedagogy, bureaucracy, ideology, and capitalism. Seminar XVII is often treated as “the political Lacan,” where the four discourses become central.  
  
### 26. The Psychoanalytic Reading Method  
  
Psychoanalytic reading should not become amateur diagnosis. The task is not to label characters, authors, or people as pathological. The task is to analyze **structure**.  
  
A mature psychoanalytic reading asks:  
  
**What image of coherence is being defended?**  
(什么连贯性形象正在被防御？)  
  
**What signifier keeps returning?**  
(什么能指反复返回？)  
  
**What desire is displaced into another object?**  
(什么欲望被转移到另一个对象上？)  
  
**What lack organizes the scene?**  
(什么缺失组织了这个场景？)  
  
**What fantasy tells the subject how to desire?**  
(什么幻想教主体如何欲望？)  
  
**Where does language fail and the Real intrude?**  
(语言在哪里失败，而实在界在哪里闯入？)  
  
In a literary context, a Lacanian writer should not mainly ask “what is my character’s diagnosis?” but rather ask what self-image the character defends, what law or institution speaks through them, what object organizes their wanting, where language fails them, and what rupture reveals that failure.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Psychoanalytic reading analyzes not personality labels, but the structure of desire, fantasy, symptom, and speech. (精神分析式阅读分析的不是人格标签，而是欲望、幻想、症状和言说的结构。)  
  
### 27. The Tool-Map of Psychoanalysis and Lacan  
  
Use psychoanalytic vocabulary diagnostically. The core question is usually not “what does the subject consciously intend?” but “what unconscious structure organizes this speech, desire, and repetition?”  
  
**If the text shows self-division**, look for **Unconscious (无意识; de: Unbewusste; fr: inconscient)**, **Repression (压抑; de: Verdrängung)**, and **Barred Subject (分裂主体; fr: sujet barré)**.  
(如果文本显示自我分裂，应寻找无意识、压抑和分裂主体问题。)  
  
**If the text shows meaningful suffering**, look for **Symptom (症状; fr: symptôme)** and **Return of the Repressed (被压抑者的返回; de: Wiederkehr des Verdrängten)**.  
(如果文本显示有意义的痛苦，应寻找症状与被压抑者返回问题。)  
  
**If the text shows repeated failure or compulsion**, look for **Drive (驱力; de: Trieb)** and **Repetition Compulsion (重复强迫; de: Wiederholungszwang)**.  
(如果文本显示重复性失败或强迫，应寻找驱力和重复强迫问题。)  
  
**If the text shows relational repetition**, look for **Transference (移情; de: Übertragung)**.  
(如果文本显示关系中的重复，应寻找移情问题。)  
  
**If the text shows self-image, rivalry, or alienated unity**, look for **Mirror Stage (镜像阶段; fr: stade du miroir)** and **Imaginary (想象界; fr: Imaginaire)**.  
(如果文本显示自我形象、竞争或异化性统一，应寻找镜像阶段和想象界问题。)  
  
**If the text shows law, language, names, and positions**, look for **Symbolic (象征界; fr: Symbolique)**, **Other (大他者; fr: grand Autre)**, **Signifier (能指; fr: signifiant)**, and **Name-of-the-Father (父名; fr: Nom-du-Père)**.  
(如果文本显示律法、语言、名称和位置，应寻找象征界、大他者、能指和父名问题。)  
  
**If the text shows rupture, trauma, or unsayability**, look for **Real (实在界; fr: Réel)**.  
(如果文本显示断裂、创伤或不可言说性，应寻找实在界问题。)  
  
**If the text shows wanting that no object satisfies**, look for **Desire (欲望; fr: désir)**, **Lack (缺失; fr: manque)**, and **objet petit a (小客体 a; fr: objet petit a)**.  
(如果文本显示没有对象能够满足的想要，应寻找欲望、缺失和小客体 a 问题。)  
  
**If the text shows painful enjoyment**, look for **Jouissance (享乐; fr: jouissance)**.  
(如果文本显示痛苦的满足，应寻找享乐问题。)  
  
**If the text shows a recurrent scene of desire**, look for **Fantasy (幻想; fr: fantasme)**.  
(如果文本显示欲望的重复性场景，应寻找幻想问题。)  
  
**If the text’s speech performs something different from what it states**, look for **Enunciation (言说行为; fr: énonciation)** and **Enunciated (所言内容; fr: énoncé)**.  
(如果文本的言说行为执行了不同于所言内容的东西，应寻找言说行为与所言内容问题。)  
  
**If the text analyzes institutional speech and social bonds**, look for **Four Discourses (四种话语; fr: quatre discours)**.  
(如果文本分析制度性言说与社会纽带，应寻找四种话语问题。)  
  
### 28. The Genealogical Point of Part 15  
  
Psychoanalysis and Lacan transform the philosophical language of the subject. Greek philosophy sought order through **logos**. Latin metaphysics stabilized essence and soul. Descartes grounded certainty in the **cogito**. Kant centered transcendental subjectivity. Hegel made subjectivity social and historical. Marx and Nietzsche made consciousness suspicious. Phenomenology returned to lived experience. Heidegger made Dasein finite and world-involved. Existentialism made freedom responsible. Structuralism displaced the subject into language. Foucault made subjectivity an effect of power/knowledge. Derrida showed that meaning is never fully present.  
  
Psychoanalysis adds:  
  
**The subject is divided by unconscious desire and spoken by signifiers it does not master.**  
(主体被无意识欲望分裂，并被其无法掌控的能指所言说。)  
  
The guiding thesis is:  
  
**Psychoanalytic and Lacanian language turns subjectivity into a problem of unconscious structure: to understand a subject is to ask what image it identifies with, what signifier represents it, what lack organizes its desire, what fantasy stages its relation to the Other, what symptom speaks for it, and where the Real interrupts its symbolic order.**  
(精神分析与拉康式语言把主体性转化为无意识结构问题：理解一个主体，就是追问它认同什么形象，什么能指代表它，什么缺失组织其欲望，什么幻想安排它同大他者的关系，什么症状替它说话，以及实在界在哪里打断其象征秩序。)  
  
This grammar is indispensable for reading literature, law, ideology, sexuality, gender, religion, political fantasy, nationalism, media desire, and clinical speech. It does not replace social critique or textual analysis. It adds the libidinal and unconscious dimension that those approaches often miss.  
  
The Lacanian question remains one of the strongest tools for philosophical reading:  
  
**What does this subject say it wants, what lack actually organizes that wanting, and what signifier or fantasy keeps the desire in motion?**  
(这个主体声称自己想要什么？实际上是什么缺失组织了这种想要？又是什么能指或幻想使欲望持续运动？)  
  
## Part 16. Feminism, Gender, and Queer Theory: Body, Sex, Performativity  
  
This chapter explains feminist, gender, and queer theory as a reorganization of philosophical language around **embodiment**, **sexual difference**, **social reproduction**, **normativity**, **performativity**, and **intersectional power**. Earlier chapters analyzed subjectivity through freedom, Being, language, discourse, power, deconstruction, and unconscious desire. Feminist and queer theory ask a sharper question: **whose body, whose labor, whose desire, whose vulnerability, and whose experience was silently treated as secondary when philosophy spoke in universal terms?** (当哲学以普遍术语说话时，谁的身体、谁的劳动、谁的欲望、谁的脆弱性和谁的经验被默默视为次要？)  
  
The central vocabulary is **Feminism**, **Patriarchy**, **Sex**, **Gender**, **Woman as Other**, **Body**, **Embodiment**, **Sexual Difference**, **Social Reproduction**, **Care**, **Domestic Labor**, **Reproductive Labor**, **Standpoint Epistemology**, **Situated Knowledge**, **Intersectionality**, **Performativity**, **Heteronormativity**, **Queer**, **Compulsory Heterosexuality**, **Male Gaze**, **Objectification**, **Agency**, and **Coalition**. Feminism is not an added “women’s issue,” but a correction of theory itself: traditional theory often universalizes male experience, marginalizes family, body, sexuality, birth, care, and emotional labor, and treats private life as outside social structure.  
  
The operational function of this chapter is precise: use feminist and queer vocabulary when the problem is **how bodies, identities, labor, desire, and knowledge are organized by gendered, sexual, racial, classed, colonial, and institutional norms**. (当问题是身体、身份、劳动、欲望和知识如何被性别化、性化、种族化、阶级化、殖民化和制度化规范组织时，应使用女性主义与酷儿理论词汇。)  
  
### 1. The Problem-Situation: The Universal Subject Was Not Neutral  
  
Classical philosophy often speaks in universal terms: **man**, **reason**, **citizen**, **subject**, **person**, **freedom**, **labor**, **knowledge**, **body**, **justice**. Feminist theory asks whether these terms were ever neutral. When philosophy said “man,” did it mean humanity, or did it smuggle in a male norm? When political theory said “citizen,” who was excluded from public life? When ethics said “autonomy,” who performed the care work that made autonomy materially possible? When epistemology imagined a neutral knower, whose social position was being erased?  
  
The central feminist question is:  
  
**What appears universal only because the labor, body, and exclusion that support it have been hidden?**  
(什么东西之所以显得普遍，只是因为支撑它的劳动、身体和排除被隐藏了？)  
  
Queer theory extends the challenge:  
  
**What appears natural only because repeated norms have made it look inevitable?**  
(什么东西之所以显得自然，只是因为重复的规范使它看起来不可避免？)  
  
This transforms philosophical reading. A concept is not only judged by its internal logic. It must also be asked: whose experience does it center? whose labor does it presuppose? whose body does it regulate? whose desire does it normalize? whose suffering does it privatize?  
  
**Typical sentence:** Feminist theory does not merely add women to philosophy; it asks how philosophy’s universal subject was historically gendered. (女性主义理论并不只是把女性加入哲学；它追问哲学的普遍主体如何在历史上被性别化。)  
  
### 2. Feminism: The Problem of Theory’s Hidden Subject  
  
`Feminism (女性主义; fr: féminisme; en: feminism)`  
**Definition:** a set of theoretical, political, and ethical projects that analyze and contest gendered domination, sexual hierarchy, embodied inequality, and the exclusion of women and gendered others from full social, political, and epistemic standing. (一组理论、政治与伦理工程，它分析并反抗性别化支配、性等级、身体化不平等，以及女性和性别化他者被排除在完整社会、政治与认识地位之外的状态。)  
**Problem solved:** it reveals that supposedly neutral theories often rely on gendered exclusions. (它揭示所谓中立理论常依赖性别化排除。)  
**Why needed:** concepts such as freedom, labor, reason, citizenship, justice, and knowledge have often been built around male-coded experience. (自由、劳动、理性、公民身份、正义和知识等概念常围绕男性化经验建构。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing gendered power, bodily regulation, social reproduction, epistemic exclusion, sexual hierarchy, or the politics of private life. (当分析性别化权力、身体规制、社会再生产、认识排除、性等级或私人生活政治时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Feminism is not one doctrine. Liberal feminism emphasizes rights, equality, education, property, and legal standing. Marxist and socialist feminism analyze labor, capitalism, reproduction, and the family. Radical feminism analyzes patriarchy, sexuality, violence, and male power. Black feminism, postcolonial feminism, indigenous feminism, trans feminism, and queer feminism criticize any feminism that treats one group’s experience as universal.  
  
The point is not merely additive: feminism is not an “added chapter” after classical theory; it rewrites social theory by asking who performs unpaid domestic labor, who cares for children and elders, whose body is managed by beauty, medicine, and the state, who bears marriage penalties, who faces sexual violence, and who is excluded from public space.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Feminism turns private life into a political and theoretical problem. (女性主义把私人生活转化为政治和理论问题。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Equality (平等; fr: égalité)** asks whether persons are treated alike; **Feminism (女性主义; fr: féminisme)** asks why the standard of equal treatment was often built from a male norm. (平等追问人是否被同等对待；女性主义追问平等对待的标准为何常由男性规范构成。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** feminism transforms the history of reason by showing that reason’s supposed universality was often supported by gendered exclusions of body, dependency, care, emotion, and reproduction. (女性主义改造理性史，显示理性所谓的普遍性常由对身体、依赖、照护、情感和生育的性别化排除支撑。)  
  
### 3. Patriarchy: The Problem of Gendered Rule  
  
`Patriarchy (父权制; el: πατήρ + ἀρχή; en: patriarchy)`  
**Definition:** a social order in which masculine authority, male-coded power, and gender hierarchy organize family, law, labor, sexuality, knowledge, and public life. (一种社会秩序，其中男性权威、男性化权力和性别等级组织家庭、法律、劳动、性、知识和公共生活。)  
**Problem solved:** it names gender domination as structural rather than merely personal prejudice. (它把性别支配命名为结构性问题，而不只是个人偏见。)  
**Why needed:** gender inequality persists through institutions, norms, inheritance, violence, labor division, symbolic authority, and bodily regulation. (性别不平等通过制度、规范、继承、暴力、劳动分工、象征权威和身体规制持续存在。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing how male authority or masculine norms are institutionalized. (当分析男性权威或男性化规范如何被制度化时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Patriarchy does not mean every man individually dominates every woman. It means social arrangements can systematically privilege masculinity, male authority, heterosexual family structure, and gendered labor division. A patriarchal system can operate through law, religion, medicine, market, school, household, media, and ordinary expectation.  
  
This is why feminism does not only criticize “bad attitudes.” It analyzes structures. A woman’s unequal burden in marriage, care work, beauty labor, workplace advancement, reproductive responsibility, or public safety is not merely personal misfortune. It belongs to social organization.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Patriarchy is not only male prejudice; it is the institutional organization of gendered power. (父权制不只是男性偏见，而是性别化权力的制度组织。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Sexism (性别歧视; en: sexism)** can refer to prejudicial belief or conduct; **Patriarchy (父权制; en: patriarchy)** names the structural order that makes such belief and conduct socially effective. (性别歧视可以指偏见性信念或行为；父权制命名使这些信念和行为具有社会效力的结构秩序。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** patriarchy turns domination inside the family, sexuality, reproduction, and private life into objects of political analysis. (父权制把家庭、性、生育和私人生活内部的支配转化为政治分析对象。)  
  
### 4. Woman as Other: The Problem of Male Universalism  
  
`Woman as Other (女人作为他者; fr: femme comme Autre)`  
**Definition:** the structure by which man is treated as universal subject while woman is positioned as deviation, complement, object, body, or relative being. (一种结构，其中男人被视为普遍主体，而女人被定位为偏差、补充、对象、身体或关系性存在。)  
**Problem solved:** it exposes how universality can be gendered. (它揭示普遍性如何可能被性别化。)  
**Why needed:** women have often been defined not as autonomous subjects, but in relation to men: wife, mother, muse, body, temptation, nature, lack, or support. (女性常不是被定义为自主主体，而是相对于男性被定义为妻子、母亲、缪斯、身体、诱惑、自然、缺失或支撑。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing asymmetry between the male-coded universal and the feminized particular. (当分析男性化普遍者与女性化特殊者之间的不对称时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
This concept is central to Simone de Beauvoir’s existential feminism. The male position appears as neutral humanity. Woman becomes the marked term. He is subject; she is other. He is transcendence; she is immanence. He is mind; she is body. He is activity; she is passivity.  
  
The point is not merely representational. Being made Other shapes education, desire, marriage, labor, sexuality, and self-understanding. It also explains why “universal human” theories may secretly describe only one gendered position.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Woman is made Other when man occupies the position of neutral human subject. (当男人占据中立人类主体的位置时，女人就被制造为他者。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Difference (差异; fr: différence)** can be symmetrical; **Othering (他者化; en: othering)** makes one term the norm and the other derivative or inferior. (差异可以是对称的；他者化使一项成为规范，另一项成为派生或低等者。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** woman-as-Other links Hegelian recognition, existential freedom, and feminist critique. Subjectivity becomes gendered through asymmetrical recognition. (女人作为他者把黑格尔式承认、存在主义自由和女性主义批判连接起来。主体性通过不对称承认而被性别化。)  
  
### 5. Sex and Gender: The Problem of Nature and Social Meaning  
  
`Sex (生理性别; la: sexus; en: sex)`  
**Definition:** the bodily, reproductive, chromosomal, hormonal, anatomical, and medical dimensions through which bodies are classified as male, female, intersex, or otherwise sexed. (身体、生殖、染色体、激素、解剖和医学维度，身体通过这些维度被分类为男性、女性、双性或其他性化状态。)  
**Problem solved:** it identifies bodily classification without automatically deriving social destiny from it. (它识别身体分类，但不自动从中推出社会命运。)  
**Why needed:** feminist theory must distinguish bodily materiality from social prescriptions attached to bodies. (女性主义理论必须区分身体物质性与附着于身体的社会规定。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing biological classification, medicine, reproduction, intersex variation, or bodily materiality. (当分析生物分类、医学、生育、双性差异或身体物质性时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
`Gender (社会性别; en: gender)`  
**Definition:** the social, cultural, legal, symbolic, behavioral, and institutional organization of masculinity, femininity, and gendered identity. (男性气质、女性气质和性别身份的社会、文化、法律、象征、行为和制度组织。)  
**Problem solved:** it separates social role and norm from biological determinism. (它把社会角色和规范同生物决定论区分开来。)  
**Why needed:** claims such as “women are naturally caring” or “men are naturally suited to authority” often naturalize social expectations. (诸如“女性天生适合照护”或“男性天生适合权威”的说法常把社会期待自然化。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing roles, norms, identity, expectations, institutions, and social classification. (当分析角色、规范、身份、期待、制度和社会分类时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
The sex/gender distinction was a major feminist tool because it showed that many things called “natural” are socially produced. Gender norms define how bodies should move, dress, speak, desire, work, reproduce, age, and appear.  
  
Two refinements matter. First, the distinction between sex and gender helps show that gender roles such as “women should be gentle” or “men should be strong” are not simple biological facts. Second, later theory complicates the distinction by showing that sex itself is not accessed outside classification: medicine, law, treatment of intersex bodies, hormones, chromosomes, and standards of normal development all involve institutional and discursive practices. This does not deny bodily materiality; it means bodies are understood through classification, measurement, naming, medicine, and law.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Gender is not the social expression of a simple natural fact; it is a norm-governed system that interprets and organizes bodies. (社会性别不是简单自然事实的社会表达，而是解释并组织身体的规范系统。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Biological Difference (生物差异; en: biological difference)** concerns bodily variation; **Gender Norm (性别规范; en: gender norm)** prescribes what bodies should mean and do socially. (生物差异关涉身体差异；性别规范规定身体在社会上应当意味着什么、做什么。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** sex/gender analysis moves feminism from rights equality to critique of naturalization. It asks how social norms become disguised as nature. (生理性别/社会性别分析使女性主义从权利平等转向自然化批判，追问社会规范如何伪装成自然。)  
  
### 6. Body: The Problem of Naturalized Regulation  
  
`Body (身体; el: σῶμα; la: corpus; en: body)`  
**Definition:** not merely a biological object, but a lived, interpreted, regulated, desired, medicalized, sexualized, racialized, and politicized site. (不仅是生物对象，也是被生活、被解释、被规制、被欲望化、被医学化、被性化、被种族化和被政治化的位置。)  
**Problem solved:** it rejects the philosophical split in which reason is universal and body is secondary, passive, feminine, or natural. (它拒绝理性被视为普遍而身体被视为次要、被动、女性化或自然化的哲学分裂。)  
**Why needed:** bodies are managed by law, medicine, religion, family, media, market, state, and everyday norms. (身体被法律、医学、宗教、家庭、媒体、市场、国家和日常规范管理。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing reproduction, sexuality, disability, appearance, aging, violence, health, bodily autonomy, or social control. (当分析生育、性、残障、外貌、衰老、暴力、健康、身体自主或社会控制时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Feminist theory makes the body central because classical philosophy often treated embodiment as a problem to overcome. The rational subject was implicitly disembodied. But no one lives without a body. Bodies menstruate, age, give birth, suffer pain, become disabled, are desired, are judged, are classified, and are exposed to violence.  
  
Women’s bodies are especially naturalized and managed: menstruation, pregnancy, birth, breastfeeding, sexuality, appearance, and aging are deeply regulated by social norms. Reproduction may involve biological capacity, but marriage law, abortion law, maternity leave, assisted reproduction, maternal morality, population policy, contraception responsibility, obstetric medicine, and family expectation are social institutions, not natural facts.  
  
**Typical sentence:** The body is not outside politics; it is one of the main surfaces on which power writes itself. (身体并不在政治之外；它是权力书写自身的主要表面之一。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Body as Object (作为对象的身体; de: Körper)** is measured and observed; **Lived Body (被生活的身体; de: Leib)** is the body through which one inhabits the world. Feminist theory adds that both are socially interpreted and politically regulated. (作为对象的身体被测量和观察；被生活的身体是人借以居住于世界的身体。女性主义进一步指出，二者都被社会解释和政治规制。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** body analysis joins phenomenology, Foucault, and feminism. The body is lived, disciplined, medicalized, gendered, racialized, and made into a site of rights and vulnerability. (身体分析连接现象学、福柯和女性主义。身体既被生活，也被规训、医学化、性别化、种族化，并成为权利与脆弱性的场所。)  
  
### 7. Embodiment: The Problem of Situated Subjectivity  
  
`Embodiment (具身性; de: Leiblichkeit; fr: corporéité; en: embodiment)`  
**Definition:** the condition that subjectivity, knowledge, agency, and experience occur through a body situated in social and material relations. (主体性、知识、行动者性和经验通过处于社会与物质关系中的身体发生的条件。)  
**Problem solved:** it rejects the fantasy of a view from nowhere and a subject without body. (它拒绝无处之视角和无身体主体的幻想。)  
**Why needed:** social position, vulnerability, perception, pain, desire, mobility, and risk are bodily as well as symbolic. (社会位置、脆弱性、知觉、痛苦、欲望、行动能力和风险既是身体性的，也是象征性的。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing how bodies mediate knowledge, freedom, constraint, agency, and social recognition. (当分析身体如何中介知识、自由、限制、行动者性和社会承认时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Embodiment is not merely “having a body.” It means that knowledge and freedom are never purely abstract. A pregnant body, disabled body, racialized body, trans body, aging body, sexually objectified body, working body, or medically monitored body does not inhabit the same world under the same conditions.  
  
This matters for ethics and politics. Bodily autonomy cannot be reduced to private choice. It requires medical access, legal protection, public safety, anti-violence structures, labor rights, reproductive justice, and social respect.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Embodiment means that freedom is lived through bodies that are differently exposed, recognized, and regulated. (具身性意味着自由通过被不同程度暴露、承认和规制的身体被生活。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Abstract Subject (抽象主体; en: abstract subject)** appears detachable from body and history; **Embodied Subject (具身主体; en: embodied subject)** exists through bodily vulnerability, capacity, and social interpretation. (抽象主体显得可脱离身体和历史；具身主体通过身体脆弱性、能力和社会解释而存在。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** embodiment transforms autonomy. Freedom is not only rational self-legislation; it is the socially supported capacity to live, move, desire, refuse, reproduce, heal, and appear bodily. (具身性改造自主性。自由不只是理性自我立法，而是由社会支持的身体性能力：生活、移动、欲望、拒绝、生育、疗愈和显现。)  
  
### 8. Social Reproduction: The Problem of Hidden Labor  
  
`Social Reproduction (社会再生产; en: social reproduction)`  
**Definition:** the labor, institutions, and practices that reproduce life, labor-power, social relations, care, households, bodies, and future generations. (再生产生命、劳动力、社会关系、照护、家庭、身体和未来世代的劳动、制度与实践。)  
**Problem solved:** it reveals the hidden work that makes market, state, and public life possible. (它揭示使市场、国家和公共生活成为可能的隐藏劳动。)  
**Why needed:** capitalism and public life depend on unpaid or underpaid care, domestic labor, emotional labor, birth, education, health, and household maintenance. (资本主义和公共生活依赖无偿或低酬照护、家务劳动、情绪劳动、生育、教育、健康和家庭维持。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing family, care, domestic work, education, health, welfare, migration, reproduction, and labor-power. (当分析家庭、照护、家务、教育、健康、福利、迁移、生育和劳动力时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Classical political economy often centers production: factory, wage, commodity, capital, market. Feminism asks how workers arrive at the factory alive, fed, raised, educated, emotionally sustained, and able to work again tomorrow. The answer is social reproduction.  
  
Family is not a warm refuge outside the market, but a core institution of social reproduction; unpaid housework, care labor, marriage, childrearing, eldercare, and cultural capital transmission support market and state functioning while transferring the costs of capitalism, patriarchy, and class inequality onto women.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Social reproduction names the labor that reproduces the conditions under which wage labor and public life can exist. (社会再生产命名再生产工资劳动与公共生活存在条件的劳动。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Production (生产; la: productio)** makes commodities or outputs; **Social Reproduction (社会再生产; en: social reproduction)** maintains people, capacities, relations, and life processes. (生产制造商品或产出；社会再生产维持人、能力、关系和生命过程。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** social reproduction theory revises Marxism by showing that capital depends not only on wage labor, but also on gendered care and domestic labor often placed outside value’s official accounting. (社会再生产理论修正马克思主义，显示资本不仅依赖工资劳动，也依赖常被置于价值正式计算之外的性别化照护和家务劳动。)  
  
### 9. Care: The Problem of Dependency and Moral Labor  
  
`Care (照护; en: care; fr: soin)`  
**Definition:** the practical, emotional, bodily, and relational labor of sustaining vulnerable, dependent, growing, aging, ill, or ordinary human life. (维持脆弱、依赖、成长、衰老、患病或普通人类生活的实践性、情感性、身体性和关系性劳动。)  
**Problem solved:** it challenges ethical and political theories that treat dependence as marginal. (它挑战把依赖视为边缘问题的伦理和政治理论。)  
**Why needed:** all human beings depend on care at birth, illness, disability, aging, crisis, and often in everyday life. (所有人在出生、疾病、残障、衰老、危机以及许多日常生活中都依赖照护。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing dependency, family, nursing, parenting, eldercare, disability, affective labor, or welfare. (当分析依赖、家庭、护理、育儿、养老、残障、情感劳动或福利时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Care exposes a weakness in liberal individualism. The autonomous individual is often imagined as self-sufficient. But self-sufficiency is produced by care work, often done by women, migrants, racialized workers, low-wage workers, or family members without recognition.  
  
Care is not merely sentiment. It is material labor, time, skill, attention, bodily effort, emotional regulation, and institutional responsibility.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Care reveals that autonomy is not the opposite of dependency; autonomy is often made possible by dependency relations that have been organized well or badly. (照护显示自主性不是依赖的反面；自主性常由被良好或糟糕组织的依赖关系所使能。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Independence (独立; en: independence)** suggests not needing others; **Relational Autonomy (关系性自主; en: relational autonomy)** understands autonomy as socially and materially supported. (独立暗示不需要他人；关系性自主把自主理解为由社会和物质条件支持。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** care ethics and feminist social theory move ethics from abstract rule, utility, or rights alone toward vulnerability, dependency, maintenance, and relational responsibility. (照护伦理和女性主义社会理论把伦理从抽象规则、效用或权利转向脆弱性、依赖、维持和关系责任。)  
  
### 10. Domestic Labor and Emotional Labor: The Problem of Invisible Work  
  
`Domestic Labor (家务劳动; en: domestic labor)`  
**Definition:** the unpaid or underpaid labor of cooking, cleaning, childcare, eldercare, household maintenance, and daily life reproduction. (烹饪、清洁、育儿、养老、家庭维护和日常生活再生产中的无偿或低酬劳动。)  
**Problem solved:** it reveals labor hidden by the public/private divide. (它揭示被公共/私人区分隐藏的劳动。)  
**Why needed:** households are productive sites even when their labor is not counted as wage labor. (家庭即使其劳动不被计为工资劳动，也仍是生产性场所。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing gendered division of labor, unpaid work, family economy, or social reproduction. (当分析性别化劳动分工、无偿工作、家庭经济或社会再生产时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
`Emotional Labor (情绪劳动; en: emotional labor)`  
**Definition:** the management, production, and regulation of feeling as part of work, family, care, service, or social expectation. (在工作、家庭、照护、服务或社会期待中对情感进行管理、生产和规制的劳动。)  
**Problem solved:** it shows that affective regulation is labor, not merely personality. (它显示情感调节是劳动，而不只是性格。)  
**Why needed:** women and feminized workers are often expected to soothe, support, smile, absorb conflict, and maintain relational stability. (女性和女性化劳动者常被期待安抚、支持、微笑、吸收冲突并维持关系稳定。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing service work, care work, family mediation, teaching, nursing, hospitality, or workplace affect. (当分析服务劳动、照护劳动、家庭调解、教学、护理、接待或工作场所情感时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Domestic and emotional labor show that what is called “private” is economically and politically structured. If someone cleans, cooks, comforts, raises children, remembers appointments, manages kinship, performs sexual availability, and absorbs emotional crisis, that work sustains others’ public freedom.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Domestic labor and emotional labor are often invisible because they are naturalized as love, femininity, or family duty. (家务劳动和情绪劳动常常不可见，因为它们被自然化为爱、女性气质或家庭义务。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Work (工作; en: work)** is often recognized when paid; **Labor (劳动; en: labor)** in feminist analysis includes unpaid, affective, reproductive, and sustaining activity. (工作常在有薪时被承认；女性主义分析中的劳动包括无偿、情感性、再生产性和维持性活动。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** labor theory expands from factory and wage to home, affect, body, reproduction, and care. (劳动理论从工厂和工资扩展到家庭、情感、身体、再生产和照护。)  
  
### 11. Bodily Autonomy: The Problem of Control over Embodied Life  
  
`Bodily Autonomy (身体自主; en: bodily autonomy)`  
**Definition:** the capacity and right to make meaningful decisions about one’s body, reproduction, sexuality, health, movement, appearance, and bodily integrity. (就自身身体、生育、性、健康、移动、外貌和身体完整性作出有意义决定的能力与权利。)  
**Problem solved:** it names freedom at the level of embodied existence rather than abstract choice alone. (它在具身存在层面命名自由，而不只是抽象选择。)  
**Why needed:** bodies are governed by law, medicine, family, violence, market, religion, platform visibility, and state policy. (身体被法律、医学、家庭、暴力、市场、宗教、平台可见性和国家政策治理。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing abortion, contraception, pregnancy, sexual consent, gender transition, disability, medical authority, violence, public safety, or bodily privacy. (当分析堕胎、避孕、怀孕、性同意、性别转变、残障、医学权威、暴力、公共安全或身体隐私时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Bodily autonomy is not an isolated private preference. It depends on institutions: healthcare, law, public safety, anti-violence protection, disability access, reproductive justice, labor policy, and cultural respect. A formal right can be hollow if medical access, money, safety, or legal protection is absent.  
  
Bodily autonomy is not an isolated personal choice; it requires law, medicine, public safety, platform governance, care systems, and cultural respect as conditions.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Bodily autonomy requires not only formal permission, but material and institutional conditions under which bodily choice can be real. (身体自主不只需要形式许可，也需要身体选择能够成为现实的物质和制度条件。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Choice (选择; en: choice)** can be abstract; **Bodily Autonomy (身体自主; en: bodily autonomy)** requires embodied capacity, safety, access, and institutional support. (选择可以是抽象的；身体自主需要具身能力、安全、可及性和制度支持。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** autonomy becomes embodied. Freedom is measured not only by what a subject may formally choose, but by what a body can safely and materially do. (自主性变得具身化。自由不仅由主体形式上可以选择什么衡量，也由身体能够安全且物质地做什么衡量。)  
  
### 12. Standpoint Epistemology: The Problem of Situated Knowing  
  
`Standpoint Epistemology (立场认识论; en: standpoint epistemology)`  
**Definition:** the view that social position shapes what one can see, know, question, and misrecognize, and that marginalized standpoints can reveal blind spots in dominant knowledge. (一种观点，认为社会位置塑造人能看见、知道、提问和误认什么，而边缘化立场能够揭示主导知识的盲点。)  
**Problem solved:** it challenges the ideal of a disembodied, positionless knower. (它挑战无身体、无位置认知者的理想。)  
**Why needed:** knowledge is produced from social locations that shape visibility and ignorance. (知识从社会位置中被生产，而社会位置塑造可见性与无知。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing who knows, from where, under what conditions, and with what blind spots. (当分析谁在认识、从哪里认识、在什么条件下认识以及带有什么盲点时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Standpoint epistemology does not mean “the oppressed are automatically correct.” It means that social position affects visibility. Those who live at the margins of dominant institutions may see contradictions that dominant groups can ignore. Experience does not replace evidence or argument, but it can reveal what official concepts fail to register.  
  
Feminist epistemology criticizes the traditional ideal knower as positionless, bodiless, affectless, and ahistorical; standpoint epistemology means social position affects visibility, and some experiences can reveal blind spots in dominant concepts, such as gender bias in medicine or supposed neutrality in policing.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Standpoint epistemology asks how social position shapes both knowledge and ignorance. (立场认识论追问社会位置如何同时塑造知识与无知。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Subjective Opinion (主观意见; en: subjective opinion)** is personal belief; **Standpoint (立场; en: standpoint)** is a socially structured position that shapes epistemic access. (主观意见是个人信念；立场是塑造认识通达的社会结构位置。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** epistemology becomes political without becoming mere relativism. The question is not only whether a claim is justified, but whose experience and institutional position made the claim visible or invisible. (认识论变得政治化，但并不变成单纯相对主义。问题不只是一个主张是否被证成，也是谁的经验和制度位置使该主张可见或不可见。)  
  
### 13. Situated Knowledge: The Problem of Objectivity after Neutrality  
  
`Situated Knowledge (处境化知识; en: situated knowledge)`  
**Definition:** knowledge produced from embodied, historical, social, and material positions rather than from a view from nowhere. (从具身的、历史的、社会的和物质的位置中生产出来的知识，而非来自无处之视角。)  
**Problem solved:** it preserves objectivity while rejecting false neutrality. (它在拒绝虚假中立的同时保留客观性。)  
**Why needed:** all knowing occurs from somewhere, but not all positions are equally accountable or equally blind. (一切认识都从某处发生，但并非所有位置都同样可问责或同样盲目。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing research, testimony, expertise, science, law, medicine, ethnography, or political knowledge. (当分析研究、证词、专业知识、科学、法律、医学、民族志或政治知识时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Situated knowledge differs from “anything goes.” It demands more accountability, not less. The knower must state position, method, limits, interest, relation to the object, and forms of exclusion. False neutrality hides these conditions. Situated objectivity makes them available for critique.  
  
This concept is especially important for law, medicine, science, and social research. The question is not only “is the claim true?” but “what apparatus made this claim visible, whose testimony counted, and whose experience was dismissed?”  
  
**Typical sentence:** Situated knowledge rejects the fiction of neutral nowhere while demanding stronger accountability for where knowledge comes from. (处境化知识拒绝中立无处之地的虚构，同时要求更强地说明知识从何处来。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Neutrality (中立; en: neutrality)** claims no position; **Situated Objectivity (处境化客观性; en: situated objectivity)** makes position explicit and accountable. (中立声称没有位置；处境化客观性使位置变得明确且可问责。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** objectivity is reconstructed. It no longer means escaping all standpoint, but building more responsible relations among standpoints, evidence, and critique. (客观性被重构。它不再意味着逃离一切立场，而是建立立场、证据和批判之间更负责任的关系。)  
  
### 14. Intersectionality: The Problem of Non-Single-Axis Power  
  
`Intersectionality (交叉性; en: intersectionality)`  
**Definition:** an analytic framework showing how gender, race, class, sexuality, disability, nationality, religion, colonial position, age, and other structures interlock to produce specific forms of inequality. (一种分析框架，显示性别、种族、阶级、性、残障、国籍、宗教、殖民位置、年龄和其他结构如何交织，生产特定形式的不平等。)  
**Problem solved:** it prevents one group’s experience from being falsely universalized. (它防止某一群体经验被错误地普遍化。)  
**Why needed:** oppression is not simply additive; structures interact and transform one another in concrete situations. (压迫不是简单相加；结构在具体处境中相互作用并相互改变。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing how multiple power structures produce a position that cannot be explained by one axis alone. (当分析多个权力结构如何生产一种无法由单一轴线解释的位置时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Intersectionality is strongly associated with **Kimberlé Crenshaw** and Black feminist legal critique. Intersectionality is not “adding more identities.” It analyzes how structures interweave: Black women’s oppression cannot be reduced to Black men’s racial experience plus white women’s gender experience; a rural migrant domestic worker’s situation cannot be separated into gender, class, migration, education, and employer-family power as if these were independent layers.  
  
This is a methodological correction. Theory must not abstract too quickly. “Women’s freedom” may mean education, freedom from domestic violence, equal pay, reproductive autonomy, protection from racialized policing, migration status security, religious dress choice, recognition of sexual minorities, or disability access depending on situation. A single model cannot replace concrete analysis.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Intersectionality asks not only whether women are oppressed, but which women, through which structures, in which institutional and historical positions. (交叉性不只追问女性是否受压迫，而是追问哪些女性、通过哪些结构、处于哪些制度和历史位置中受压迫。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Identity Politics (身份政治; en: identity politics)** politicizes group-based exclusion; **Intersectionality (交叉性; en: intersectionality)** corrects identity politics by showing that identities are internally differentiated and structurally interwoven. (身份政治使群体性排除政治化；交叉性通过显示身份内部差异和结构交织来修正身份政治。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** intersectionality transforms feminism, race theory, legal theory, disability studies, queer theory, and postcolonial theory by refusing any single default subject. (交叉性通过拒绝任何单一默认主体，改造女性主义、种族理论、法理论、残障研究、酷儿理论和后殖民理论。)  
  
### 15. Performativity: The Problem of Gender as Repeated Act  
  
`Performativity (施行性/表演性; en: performativity)`  
**Definition:** the capacity of utterances, repeated acts, norms, or practices to produce effects rather than merely represent a prior reality. (话语、重复行为、规范或实践生产效果的能力，而不只是再现一个先在现实。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains gender not as inner essence simply expressed outward, but as repeated social production. (它把性别解释为重复性社会生产，而不是内在本质的外在表达。)  
**Why needed:** what appears natural may be the effect of ritualized repetition. (显得自然的东西可能是仪式化重复的效果。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing gesture, dress, voice, bodily style, role, norm, citation, identity, and the repetition that makes gender appear real. (当分析姿态、服饰、声音、身体风格、角色、规范、引用、身份，以及使性别显得真实的重复时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
**Usage layers:**  
1. **Speech-act use (言语行为理论用法):** in Austin and speech act theory, **performativity** concerns utterances that do something in being said, such as promising, naming, declaring, sentencing, or marrying. (在奥斯汀和言语行为理论中，施行性关涉“说出即做出某事”的话语，例如承诺、命名、宣布、宣判或缔结婚姻。)  
  
2. **Butlerian gender-theory use (巴特勒式性别理论用法):** in Butler, gender performativity does not mean voluntary theatrical performance. It means the repeated citation of norms through which gendered subjects become socially intelligible. (在巴特勒那里，性别表演性不是自愿的戏剧表演，而是规范通过重复引用而使性别主体成为社会可理解者的过程。)
