3. **Contemporary transferable use (当代理论泛用法):** in social theory, law, media studies, and cultural criticism, performativity may describe how repeated practices, metrics, classifications, protocols, or declarations produce the realities they appear merely to describe. (在社会理论、法学、媒介研究和文化批评中，表演性可指重复实践、指标、分类、协议或宣告如何生产它们似乎只是在描述的现实。)  
  
**Transfer rule:** use **performativity** when repetition, norm, utterance, or practice helps produce the reality it names. Do not use it as a synonym for performance, hypocrisy, acting, or self-expression. (转用规则：当重复、规范、话语或实践参与生产其所命名的现实，才使用 performativity。不要把它当成 performance、虚伪、演戏或自我表达的同义词。)  
  
**Do not confuse with:** performance, theatricality, role-playing, expression, representation.  
  
Performativity is associated with **Judith Butler**. It does not mean that gender is a free theatrical performance chosen at will. It means that gender is produced through repeated acts under constraint. The subject does not stand outside gender norms and choose them like costumes. The subject becomes recognizable through norms that precede it.  
  
This concept joins Derrida and Foucault. From Derrida, performativity inherits iterability: acts can be repeated and altered. From Foucault, it inherits normativity and subjectivation: subjects are produced through regulatory practices.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Gender performativity means that gender appears natural because it is repeatedly enacted, cited, and sedimented under social norms. (性别表演性意味着性别之所以显得自然，是因为它在社会规范下被反复施行、引用和沉积。)   
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Performance (表演; en: performance)** can suggest conscious theatrical display; **Performativity (表演性; en: performativity)** names the constitutive repetition through which identity is produced. (表演可能暗示有意识的戏剧展示；表演性命名身份借以被生产的构成性重复。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** gender becomes a citational practice. It is not a hidden essence behind acts, but the sedimented effect of repeated norms. (性别成为一种引用性实践。它不是行为背后的隐藏本质，而是规范重复沉积下来的效果。)  
  
### 16. Heteronormativity: The Problem of Normalized Desire  
  
`Heteronormativity (异性恋规范性; en: heteronormativity)`  
**Definition:** the social order that treats heterosexuality, binary gender, reproductive couplehood, and male/female complementarity as natural, normal, and privileged. (一种社会秩序，它把异性恋、二元性别、生殖性伴侣关系和男女互补视为自然、正常且优先。)  
**Problem solved:** it reveals heterosexuality as a norm-governed institution rather than merely private preference. (它揭示异性恋不仅是私人偏好，也是由规范支配的制度。)  
**Why needed:** sexuality is organized through law, family, medicine, education, religion, media, and state policy. (性通过法律、家庭、医学、教育、宗教、媒体和国家政策被组织。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing marriage, family, sexuality, school norms, medical categories, public culture, or legal recognition. (当分析婚姻、家庭、性、学校规范、医学分类、公共文化或法律承认时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Heteronormativity does not mean that every heterosexual person is oppressive. It means institutions often presume heterosexuality as the default. Forms, laws, families, stories, medical protocols, public rituals, and citizenship norms often assume binary sex, heterosexual coupling, reproduction, and gender complementarity.  
  
This makes non-heteronormative lives appear deviant, incomplete, excessive, immature, dangerous, or unintelligible.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Heteronormativity makes one form of desire appear natural by organizing institutions around it. (异性恋规范性通过围绕一种欲望形式组织制度，使其显得自然。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Heterosexuality (异性恋; en: heterosexuality)** can name a sexual orientation or practice; **Heteronormativity (异性恋规范性; en: heteronormativity)** names the institutional privilege of heterosexuality as norm. (异性恋可以命名性取向或实践；异性恋规范性命名异性恋作为规范的制度特权。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** sexuality becomes institutional. Desire is not only private interiority; it is organized by recognition, kinship, medicine, law, and social intelligibility. (性变得制度化。欲望不只是私人内在性，而是由承认、亲属、医学、法律和社会可理解性组织。)  
  
### 17. Queer: The Problem of Normative Disruption  
  
`Queer (酷儿; en: queer)`  
**Definition:** a critical term for non-normative sexualities, genders, practices, identities, and analytic methods that disturb fixed norms of sex, gender, and desire. (一个批判性术语，指非规范的性、性别、实践、身份，以及扰动固定性别、性和欲望规范的分析方法。)  
**Problem solved:** it resists the stabilization of identity into fixed, respectable, norm-compliant categories. (它反抗把身份稳定为固定、体面、符合规范的分类。)  
**Why needed:** even recognition politics can normalize some identities while excluding others. (即使承认政治也可能规范化某些身份，同时排除另一些身份。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing instability, non-normativity, anti-assimilation, sexual dissidence, gender variance, or critique of identity categories. (当分析不稳定性、非规范性、反同化、性异议、性别变异或身份分类批判时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Queer theory does not only ask for inclusion of LGBT identities into existing institutions. It asks how institutions define normal sexuality and recognizable gender in the first place. It is therefore both political and methodological.  
  
Queer critique asks whether the demand for respectability can reproduce hierarchy: married over unmarried, monogamous over non-monogamous, cisgender over trans, gender-conforming over gender-nonconforming, respectable sexuality over stigmatized sexuality.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Queer theory questions not only exclusion from norms, but the authority of the norm itself. (酷儿理论质疑的不只是被规范排除，也质疑规范本身的权威。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **LGBT Identity Politics (LGBT 身份政治; en: LGBT identity politics)** often seeks recognition for defined groups; **Queer Theory (酷儿理论; en: queer theory)** questions the stability and authority of the categories themselves. (LGBT 身份政治常为明确群体寻求承认；酷儿理论质疑这些分类本身的稳定性与权威。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** queer theory turns identity critique back on identity itself. It uses recognition strategically while resisting final closure around identity categories. (酷儿理论把身份批判转向身份自身。它策略性使用承认，同时抵抗围绕身份分类的最终封闭。)  
  
### 18. Compulsory Heterosexuality: The Problem of Desire as Institution  
  
`Compulsory Heterosexuality (强制性异性恋; en: compulsory heterosexuality)`  
**Definition:** the social and institutional production of heterosexuality as expected, required, natural, and economically or emotionally compulsory. (把异性恋生产为被期待、被要求、自然且在经济或情感上具有强制性的社会与制度过程。)  
**Problem solved:** it shows that heterosexuality is not merely one option among others when institutions organize survival, recognition, family, and legitimacy through it. (它显示当制度通过异性恋组织生存、承认、家庭和合法性时，异性恋并不只是诸选择之一。)  
**Why needed:** desire is shaped by material dependency, family expectation, violence, law, religion, and cultural narrative. (欲望由物质依赖、家庭期待、暴力、法律、宗教和文化叙事塑造。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing how heterosexuality becomes socially required rather than simply personally chosen. (当分析异性恋如何成为社会要求而非单纯个人选择时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
This concept is crucial because it links desire to institution. It asks how women’s dependency, marriage, family respectability, inheritance, safety, religion, and national reproduction have been organized through heterosexual norms.  
  
It also helps read literature and culture. A heterosexual romance plot may appear natural because narrative structure has trained audiences to treat it as completion.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Compulsory heterosexuality makes heterosexual desire appear freely chosen by organizing social survival around it. (强制性异性恋通过围绕异性恋组织社会生存，使异性恋欲望显得像自由选择。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Desire (欲望; fr: désir)** can appear intimate; **Compulsion (强制; en: compulsion)** shows how intimacy can be institutionally organized. (欲望可以显得亲密；强制显示亲密关系如何可能被制度组织。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** sexuality becomes a political economy of kinship, inheritance, safety, legitimacy, and social survival. (性成为亲属、继承、安全、合法性和社会生存的政治经济。)  
  
### 19. Male Gaze: The Problem of Visual Power  
  
`Male Gaze (男性凝视; en: male gaze)`  
**Definition:** a visual and representational structure that positions women or feminized bodies as objects for masculine viewing, desire, evaluation, or control. (一种视觉与表象结构，它把女性或女性化身体定位为供男性观看、欲望、评价或控制的对象。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains how visual culture organizes gendered subject and object positions. (它解释视觉文化如何组织性别化主体与对象位置。)  
**Why needed:** looking is not neutral; it can objectify, discipline, eroticize, shame, rank, and commodify bodies. (观看并不中立；它可以对象化、规训、情色化、羞辱、排序和商品化身体。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing film, advertising, pornography, fashion, social media, beauty culture, surveillance, or public space. (当分析电影、广告、色情、时尚、社交媒体、美貌文化、监视或公共空间时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
The male gaze is not simply any man looking at any woman. It is a structure. A camera, advertisement, narrative, platform, or public norm can make the viewer occupy a masculine position even when the actual viewer is not male. It organizes who looks, who is looked at, who acts, who is displayed, and whose desire counts.  
  
This connects directly to bodily autonomy and objectification. A body that is constantly evaluated becomes disciplined from within.  
  
**Typical sentence:** The male gaze turns the body into an object organized for masculine visual pleasure and judgment. (男性凝视把身体转化为为男性视觉快感和判断而组织的对象。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Seeing (看见; en: seeing)** is perceptual; **Gaze (凝视; fr: regard; en: gaze)** is structured by power, desire, and position. (看见是知觉性的；凝视由权力、欲望和位置结构化。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** visuality becomes political. Representation does not merely mirror gender; it trains gendered perception and bodily self-relation. (视觉性变得政治化。表象不只是反映性别；它训练性别化知觉和身体自我关系。)  
  
### 20. Objectification: The Problem of Being Made Thing  
  
`Objectification (对象化/物化; de: Vergegenständlichung/Verdinglichung; en: objectification)`  
**Definition:** the process by which a person is treated as an object, instrument, surface, property, commodity, body-part, or thing for another’s use or evaluation. (一个人被当作对象、工具、表面、财产、商品、身体部件或供他人使用与评价之物的过程。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains how personhood is reduced or reorganized through gendered, sexual, racial, or market relations. (它解释人格如何通过性别化、性化、种族化或市场关系被缩减或重组。)  
**Why needed:** objectification can coexist with apparent consent, visibility, admiration, or market success. (对象化可以同表面同意、可见性、欣赏或市场成功共存。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing sexualization, commodification, beauty labor, labor exploitation, racial fetishization, or bodily display. (当分析性化、商品化、美貌劳动、劳动剥削、种族恋物化或身体展示时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Objectification is not only insult. It can be pleasurable, profitable, normalized, and desired under conditions where recognition itself has been organized through objectifying standards. That is why the concept requires care. The question is not simply whether the body is visible. The question is who controls visibility, who profits, what norm governs the body, and whether agency is expanded or constrained.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Objectification occurs when a person’s subjectivity is subordinated to their function as an object for another’s use, desire, or evaluation. (当一个人的主体性从属于其作为供他人使用、欲望或评价之对象的功能时，对象化就发生了。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Embodiment (具身性; en: embodiment)** affirms bodily subjectivity; **Objectification (对象化; en: objectification)** reduces or reorganizes the person as object. (具身性肯定身体主体性；对象化把人缩减或重组为对象。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** objectification connects feminist theory with Marxian reification, Lacanian gaze, Foucaultian discipline, and media critique. (对象化把女性主义理论同马克思式物化、拉康式凝视、福柯式规训和媒介批判连接起来。)  
  
### 21. Agency: The Problem of Action under Constraint  
  
`Agency (行动者性; en: agency)`  
**Definition:** the capacity to act, interpret, resist, negotiate, choose, and transform conditions, even under constraint. (在约束之下行动、解释、抵抗、协商、选择和转化条件的能力。)  
**Problem solved:** it prevents feminist theory from reducing women and gendered subjects to passive victims. (它防止女性主义理论把女性和性别化主体化约为被动受害者。)  
**Why needed:** domination structures action, but does not erase all action. (支配结构化行动，但并不抹除一切行动。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing constrained choice, survival strategies, resistance, negotiation, complicity, refusal, or self-making. (当分析受限选择、生存策略、抵抗、协商、共谋、拒绝或自我形成时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
**Transfer rule:** use **Agency** when the issue is practical capacity to act within constraints; do not confuse it with full autonomy, sovereign control, pure freedom, or individual intention. (转用规则：当问题是在约束条件中行动的实践能力时，才使用 Agency；不要把它同完整自主、主权式控制、纯粹自由或个人意图混同。)  
  
Agency is not pure freedom. A person can act under conditions they did not choose. A woman may negotiate patriarchal family expectations. A queer subject may use norms strategically. A worker may comply, resist, delay, reinterpret, or form alliances. A trans subject may navigate medical and legal systems while also transforming them.  
  
This is why feminist theory must avoid two errors: portraying subjects as completely determined or imagining them as freely self-creating outside structure.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Agency is not action without constraint; it is the capacity to act within and against constraint. (行动者性不是没有约束的行动，而是在约束之中并反向作用于约束的能力。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Autonomy (自主性; el: αὐτός + νόμος)** emphasizes self-rule; **Agency (行动者性; en: agency)** emphasizes practical capacity to act within conditions. (自主性强调自我立法；行动者性强调在条件中行动的实践能力。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** agency becomes situated, embodied, and relational. Freedom is not abstract independence, but negotiated capacity inside power relations. (行动者性变得处境化、具身化和关系化。自由不是抽象独立，而是权力关系内部的协商性能力。)  
  
### 22. Recognition and Misrecognition: The Problem of Social Intelligibility  
  
`Recognition (承认; de: Anerkennung; en: recognition)`  
**Definition:** social confirmation of a person or group as intelligible, dignified, rights-bearing, and capable of agency. (社会对个人或群体作为可理解、有尊严、拥有权利并具有行动能力者的确认。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains why identity and freedom depend on social relations. (它解释为什么身份与自由依赖社会关系。)  
**Why needed:** gendered and sexual subjects often need recognition in law, family, medicine, language, and public space. (性别化与性化主体常需要在法律、家庭、医学、语言和公共空间中获得承认。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing gender identity, legal status, kinship, naming, rights, respect, and public visibility. (当分析性别身份、法律地位、亲属、命名、权利、尊重和公共可见性时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
`Misrecognition (误认; en: misrecognition)`  
**Definition:** a social relation in which a person or group is rendered inferior, invisible, deviant, unintelligible, or wrongly classified. (一种社会关系，其中个人或群体被制造为低等的、不可见的、异常的、不可理解的或被错误分类的存在。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains injury at the level of social meaning, not only material distribution. (它解释社会意义层面的伤害，而不只是物质分配。)  
**Why needed:** being wrongly named, erased, stereotyped, or pathologized can damage agency and social standing. (被错误命名、抹除、刻板化或病理化会损害行动者性和社会地位。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing trans recognition, racialized gender, disability, sexual stigma, legal invisibility, or symbolic harm. (当分析跨性别承认、种族化性别、残障、性污名、法律不可见性或象征伤害时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Recognition is not merely politeness. It determines whether a person can appear as spouse, parent, citizen, patient, worker, victim, speaker, knower, or rights-bearing subject.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Misrecognition wounds by making a person socially unintelligible or intelligible only through a degrading category. (误认通过使一个人在社会上不可理解，或只能通过贬低性分类被理解，而造成伤害。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Visibility (可见性; en: visibility)** means being seen; **Recognition (承认; en: recognition)** means being seen under a category that affirms status and agency. (可见性意味着被看见；承认意味着在确认地位和行动者性的分类下被看见。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** recognition theory joins feminism, queer theory, Hegel, existentialism, and critical theory. Identity is neither purely private nor merely expressive; it is socially mediated. (承认理论连接女性主义、酷儿理论、黑格尔、存在主义和批判理论。身份既不是纯私人性的，也不只是表达性的；它被社会中介。)  
  
### 23. Coalition: The Problem of Solidarity without Sameness  
  
`Coalition (联盟; la: coalescere; en: coalition)`  
**Definition:** a political relation among differently situated groups or subjects who act together without assuming identical experience. (处境不同的群体或主体在不假设经验相同的情况下共同行动的政治关系。)  
**Problem solved:** it answers the intersectional problem of how to build politics without erasing difference. (它回应交叉性问题：如何在不抹除差异的情况下建立政治。)  
**Why needed:** no single identity can represent all forms of oppression, but isolated identities cannot transform structures alone. (没有单一身份能够代表所有压迫形式，但孤立身份也无法独自转化结构。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing feminist, queer, antiracist, labor, disability, migrant, postcolonial, or environmental alliances. (当分析女性主义、酷儿、反种族主义、劳动、残障、移民、后殖民或环境联盟时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Coalition is not the same as unity through sameness. It is not “everyone has the same experience.” It is structured alliance across difference. Intersectionality makes coalition harder, but also more necessary.  
  
A coalition politics asks: what shared target exists? what differences must not be erased? whose voice has been centered? whose risk is greatest? what institutional change can connect these struggles?  
  
**Typical sentence:** Coalition builds solidarity without requiring that all participants occupy the same position. (联盟建立不要求所有参与者处于相同位置的团结。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Universalism (普遍主义; en: universalism)** can erase difference when premature; **Coalition (联盟; en: coalition)** builds common action through acknowledged difference. (普遍主义若过早使用会抹除差异；联盟则通过被承认的差异建立共同行动。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** coalition politics is the practical answer to the critique of false universality. It seeks common struggle without returning to a single default subject. (联盟政治是对虚假普遍性批判的实践回应。它寻求共同斗争，但不回到单一默认主体。)  
  
### 24. The Feminist and Queer Diagnostic Method  
  
Feminist and queer analysis should not become a mere vocabulary of accusation. The method is more exact.  
  
A strong feminist or queer reading asks:  
  
**Who is treated as the default subject?**  
(谁被当作默认主体？)  
  
**Whose body is naturalized, regulated, or made invisible?**  
(谁的身体被自然化、规制或不可见化？)  
  
**Whose labor makes the scene possible but remains uncounted?**  
(谁的劳动使这个场景成为可能，却仍未被计算？)  
  
**What desire is normalized, and what desire is made deviant?**  
(什么欲望被规范化，什么欲望被制造为异常？)  
  
**What binary organizes the field: man/woman, public/private, reason/body, natural/artificial, normal/deviant, heterosexual/queer?**  
(什么二元对立组织了这一场域：男/女、公共/私人、理性/身体、自然/人工、正常/异常、异性恋/酷儿？)  
  
**Which differences within the category “woman,” “queer,” or “subject” are being erased?**  
(“女性”“酷儿”或“主体”分类内部的哪些差异正在被抹除？)  
  
An intersectional feminist analysis cannot only ask whether women are oppressed; it must ask which women, in what class, race, region, age, bodily condition, and institutional position.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Feminist and queer analysis asks what norm produces the subject as natural, and what labor, body, or desire that norm must hide. (女性主义与酷儿分析追问什么规范把主体生产为自然，以及该规范必须隐藏什么劳动、身体或欲望。)  
  
### 25. The Tool-Map of Feminism, Gender, and Queer Theory  
  
Use feminist and queer vocabulary diagnostically. The core question is usually not only “is this equal?” but “what gendered, sexual, bodily, and intersectional structure makes this appear natural?”  
  
**If the text treats male-coded experience as universal**, look for **Feminism (女性主义; en: feminism)**, **Woman as Other (女人作为他者; fr: femme comme Autre)**, and **Male Universalism (男性普遍主义; en: male universalism)**.  
(如果文本把男性化经验视为普遍经验，应寻找女性主义、女人作为他者和男性普遍主义问题。)  
  
**If the text analyzes structural gender domination**, look for **Patriarchy (父权制; en: patriarchy)**, **Sexism (性别歧视; en: sexism)**, and **Gender Hierarchy (性别等级; en: gender hierarchy)**.  
(如果文本分析结构性性别支配，应寻找父权制、性别歧视和性别等级问题。)  
  
**If the text distinguishes bodies from social norms**, look for **Sex (生理性别; la: sexus)**, **Gender (社会性别; en: gender)**, and **Naturalization (自然化; en: naturalization)**.  
(如果文本区分身体与社会规范，应寻找生理性别、社会性别和自然化问题。)  
  
**If the text analyzes bodily regulation**, look for **Body (身体; la: corpus)**, **Embodiment (具身性; en: embodiment)**, and **Bodily Autonomy (身体自主; en: bodily autonomy)**.  
(如果文本分析身体规制，应寻找身体、具身性和身体自主问题。)  
  
**If the text analyzes hidden labor**, look for **Social Reproduction (社会再生产; en: social reproduction)**, **Care (照护; en: care)**, **Domestic Labor (家务劳动; en: domestic labor)**, and **Emotional Labor (情绪劳动; en: emotional labor)**.  
(如果文本分析隐藏劳动，应寻找社会再生产、照护、家务劳动和情绪劳动问题。)  
  
**If the text analyzes knowledge from social position**, look for **Standpoint Epistemology (立场认识论; en: standpoint epistemology)** and **Situated Knowledge (处境化知识; en: situated knowledge)**.  
(如果文本分析来自社会位置的知识，应寻找立场认识论与处境化知识问题。)  
  
**If the text warns against universalizing one group’s experience**, look for **Intersectionality (交叉性; en: intersectionality)**.  
(如果文本警惕把某一群体经验普遍化，应寻找交叉性问题。)  
  
**If the text analyzes gender as repeated norm**, look for **Performativity (表演性; en: performativity)**.  
(如果文本把性别分析为重复性规范，应寻找表演性问题。)  
  
**If the text analyzes normalized sexuality**, look for **Heteronormativity (异性恋规范性; en: heteronormativity)** and **Compulsory Heterosexuality (强制性异性恋; en: compulsory heterosexuality)**.  
(如果文本分析被规范化的性，应寻找异性恋规范性与强制性异性恋问题。)  
  
**If the text resists stable identity categories**, look for **Queer (酷儿; en: queer)** and **Anti-Normativity (反规范性; en: anti-normativity)**.  
(如果文本抵抗稳定身份分类，应寻找酷儿与反规范性问题。)  
  
**If the text analyzes visual objectification**, look for **Male Gaze (男性凝视; en: male gaze)** and **Objectification (对象化; en: objectification)**.  
(如果文本分析视觉对象化，应寻找男性凝视和对象化问题。)  
  
**If the text analyzes politics across difference**, look for **Coalition (联盟; en: coalition)**.  
(如果文本分析跨差异政治，应寻找联盟问题。)  
  
### 26. The Genealogical Point of Part 16  
  
Feminist, gender, and queer theory transform the philosophical language of the subject, body, knowledge, and freedom. Greek and Latin metaphysics often subordinated body to reason and matter to form. Modern philosophy centered the rational subject but often imagined it without sex, dependency, domestic labor, reproductive vulnerability, racialization, disability, or sexuality. Existentialism made freedom central, but feminism asked whether freedom was equally available under marriage, motherhood, violence, economic dependency, and bodily regulation. Foucault showed how bodies and subjects are produced by power/knowledge. Derrida showed how binary hierarchies depend on excluded terms. Lacan showed that desire is structured by lack and the Other.  
  
Feminist and queer theory add:  
  
**The universal subject was gendered, embodied, sexually regulated, dependent on care, and positioned inside intersecting structures of power.**  
(普遍主体其实是被性别化的、具身的、受性规范规制的、依赖照护的，并处在交叉权力结构中的主体。)  
  
The guiding thesis is:  
  
**Feminist and queer language turns philosophy toward the hidden conditions of embodiment and normativity: to understand a subject, concept, institution, or desire is to ask whose body it assumes, whose labor it hides, whose sexuality it normalizes, whose knowledge it discredits, and which intersecting structures make some lives appear natural while others appear deviant.**  
(女性主义与酷儿语言把哲学转向具身性与规范性的隐藏条件：理解一个主体、概念、制度或欲望，就是追问它预设谁的身体，隐藏谁的劳动，规范化谁的性，贬低谁的知识，以及哪些交叉结构使某些生活显得自然、另一些生活显得异常。)  
  
This grammar prepares the next stage: **Postcolonial Theory**. Once feminism and queer theory show that the universal subject is gendered and sexually normalized, postcolonial theory asks how that subject was also racialized, imperial, colonial, linguistic, and globally positioned.  
  
The feminist-queer question remains one of the strongest tools for philosophical reading:  
  
**Whose body, labor, desire, and standpoint must be hidden or disciplined for this concept to appear universal, natural, and neutral?**  
(为了使这个概念显得普遍、自然且中立，谁的身体、劳动、欲望和立场必须被隐藏或规训？)  
  
## Part 17. Postcolonial Theory: Empire, Orientalism, Subalternity  
  
This chapter explains **Postcolonial Theory** as a critique of modernity from the side of empire. Earlier chapters showed that the universal subject was gendered, embodied, sexualized, and regulated. Postcolonial theory adds another decisive pressure: **modernity was not only European reason, democracy, science, and capitalism; it was also colonial conquest, racial classification, slavery, extraction, missionary knowledge, imperial administration, and global inequality**. (现代性不只是欧洲理性、民主、科学和资本主义；它也是殖民征服、种族分类、奴隶制、资源榨取、传教知识、帝国行政和全球不平等。)  
  
The central question is:  
  
**What becomes invisible when Europe narrates itself as the origin, standard, and destination of modern history?**  
(当欧洲把自身叙述为现代历史的起源、标准和目的地时，什么被变得不可见？)  
  
The central vocabulary is **Colonialism**, **Imperialism**, **Empire**, **Orientalism**, **Colonial Discourse**, **Othering**, **Subaltern**, **Representation**, **Voice**, **Epistemic Violence**, **Colonial Knowledge**, **Race**, **Racialization**, **Decolonization**, **Anti-Colonial Nationalism**, **Neocolonialism**, **World-System**, **Core/Periphery**, **Hybridity**, **Mimicry**, **Ambivalence**, **Diaspora**, **Creolization**, **Indigeneity**, **Settler Colonialism**, and **Decoloniality**.  
  
The basic postcolonial correction is that classical sociology often treats European modernization as an internal European process, but modern society cannot be understood apart from colonialism, slavery, imperialism, racial classification, and global inequality. Capitalism’s world market was also tied to land seizure, slave trade, colonial rule, resource extraction, forced labor, and military violence.  
  
The operational function of this chapter is exact: use postcolonial vocabulary when the problem is **how empire produces knowledge, race, space, labor, subjectivity, culture, and global hierarchy while presenting itself as civilization, progress, development, or universal reason**. (当问题是帝国如何生产知识、种族、空间、劳动、主体性、文化和全球等级，同时把自身呈现为文明、进步、发展或普遍理性时，应使用后殖民理论词汇。)  
  
### 1. The Problem-Situation: Modernity Was Imperial  
  
A standard European story says: science, Enlightenment, revolution, rights, capitalism, industry, democracy, progress. Postcolonial theory does not say this story is simply false. It says the story is incomplete and politically organized.  
  
The missing side is empire.  
  
European industrialization depended on colonial trade, plantation systems, slavery, mineral extraction, military power, shipping, finance, and uneven global markets. The modern state developed not only through citizenship and law, but also through conquest, census, border-making, colonial policing, and racial administration. Modern knowledge developed not only through reason and science, but also through maps, ethnography, philology, missionary reports, travel writing, colonial archives, and administrative classification.  
  
Modernity is often narrated as an internal European story, but European modernity was deeply connected with colonial expansion, slave trade, overseas plunder, and world-market formation.  
  
The postcolonial question is therefore:  
  
**Who paid the cost of Europe’s progress, and who was made into the object of Europe’s knowledge?**  
(谁为欧洲进步支付了代价？谁又被制造成欧洲知识的对象？)  
  
**Typical sentence:** Postcolonial theory provincializes Europe by showing that European modernity was formed through colonial and global relations, not by isolated internal development. (后殖民理论通过显示欧洲现代性是在殖民和全球关系中形成的，而非孤立内部发展，来地方化欧洲。)  
  
### 2. Colonialism: The Problem of Rule over Land, Bodies, and Knowledge  
  
`Colonialism (殖民主义; la: colonia; en: colonialism)`  
**Definition:** the political, economic, military, cultural, and epistemic domination of one territory or people by an external power. (一个外部权力对某一土地或人民进行政治、经济、军事、文化和认识论支配。)  
**Problem solved:** it names domination as territorial, administrative, racial, economic, and epistemic, not merely cultural misunderstanding. (它把支配命名为领土性的、行政性的、种族性的、经济性的和认识论的，而不只是文化误解。)  
**Why needed:** colonial rule organizes land, labor, law, education, language, sexuality, religion, and identity. (殖民统治组织土地、劳动、法律、教育、语言、性、宗教和身份。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing direct rule, settlement, extraction, administration, missionary conversion, colonial schooling, racial hierarchy, or forced labor. (当分析直接统治、定居、榨取、行政、传教改宗、殖民学校、种族等级或强迫劳动时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Colonialism is not only taking land. It restructures the world. It creates colonial borders, converts land into property, classifies populations, rewrites law, installs schools, extracts resources, and forces colonized subjects to encounter themselves through colonial categories.  
  
A colony is therefore not merely a place under foreign power. It is a laboratory of rule. The colonized person is classified, educated, taxed, policed, represented, translated, converted, studied, and often made to internalize the colonizer’s categories.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Colonialism governs by taking territory, reorganizing labor, classifying populations, and producing knowledge about the colonized. (殖民主义通过占有领土、重组劳动、分类人口并生产关于被殖民者的知识来治理。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Conquest (征服; la: conquisitio)** can name military seizure; **Colonialism (殖民主义; en: colonialism)** names the continuing system of rule, extraction, administration, and subject-formation after conquest. (征服可以指军事占领；殖民主义命名征服之后持续存在的统治、榨取、行政和主体形成系统。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** colonialism turns modernity into a global relation. The modern subject, state, market, and science are no longer purely European achievements; they are entangled with colonial domination. (殖民主义把现代性转化为全球关系。现代主体、国家、市场和科学不再只是欧洲成就，而是同殖民支配纠缠在一起。)  
  
### 3. Imperialism: The Problem of Global Power beyond Direct Rule  
  
`Imperialism (帝国主义; la: imperium; en: imperialism)`  
**Definition:** the extension of a state, capital, culture, or geopolitical power over other territories and peoples through military, economic, administrative, cultural, or financial means. (国家、资本、文化或地缘政治权力通过军事、经济、行政、文化或金融手段向其他土地和人民扩张。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains domination that may exceed formal colonial rule. (它解释超出正式殖民统治的支配。)  
**Why needed:** imperial power can continue through markets, debt, military bases, trade regimes, development policy, media, language, and knowledge institutions. (帝国权力可以通过市场、债务、军事基地、贸易体制、发展政策、媒体、语言和知识制度继续存在。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing global hierarchy, resource extraction, military dominance, financial dependency, cultural hegemony, or development regimes. (当分析全球等级、资源榨取、军事支配、金融依赖、文化霸权或发展体制时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Imperialism is broader than colonialism. Colonialism often implies direct control over territory. Imperialism can operate through indirect control. A formally independent state may still be subordinated through debt, trade rules, aid conditionality, military alignment, corporate extraction, or epistemic dependence.  
  
This is why postcolonial theory must also analyze the present. The end of formal empire does not automatically end imperial relations.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Imperialism can persist after colonial rule ends by reorganizing dependency through finance, trade, military power, and knowledge. (帝国主义可以在殖民统治结束后继续存在，通过金融、贸易、军事权力和知识重组依赖。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Colonialism (殖民主义; en: colonialism)** usually names direct rule or settlement; **Imperialism (帝国主义; en: imperialism)** names a wider structure of domination that can be direct or indirect. (殖民主义通常命名直接统治或定居；帝国主义命名更广泛的支配结构，可直接也可间接。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** imperialism links postcolonial theory with Marxism, international political economy, world-systems theory, and development critique. (帝国主义把后殖民理论同马克思主义、国际政治经济学、世界体系理论和发展批判连接起来。)  
  
### 4. Empire: The Problem of Universal Rule  
  
`Empire (帝国; la: imperium; en: empire)`  
**Definition:** a political and symbolic formation that organizes heterogeneous peoples, territories, laws, races, and economies under an expansive structure of rule. (一种政治与象征构型，它把异质人民、领土、法律、种族和经济组织到扩张性统治结构之下。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains rule across difference without assuming equal citizenship. (它解释跨差异统治，而不假设平等公民身份。)  
**Why needed:** empire often governs by differentiating subjects: citizen, native, settler, slave, migrant, protectorate subject, civilized, primitive, loyal, rebel. (帝国常通过区分主体来治理：公民、土著、定居者、奴隶、移民、保护地臣民、文明者、原始者、忠诚者、叛乱者。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing multi-territorial rule, imperial law, racial hierarchy, indirect rule, civilizing mission, or imperial citizenship. (当分析多领土统治、帝国法律、种族等级、间接统治、文明使命或帝国公民身份时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Empire does not always seek sameness. Often it governs by difference. It creates legal pluralism, racial categories, administrative zones, protectorates, native authorities, special courts, and unequal citizenship. This is one reason empire can present itself as order while preserving hierarchy.  
  
Empire also produces imagination. It tells stories of mission, destiny, civilization, security, progress, burden, and world order.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Empire rules by producing a differentiated order in which not all subjects occupy the same legal, racial, or political position. (帝国通过生产一种差异化秩序来统治，其中并非所有主体都占据相同的法律、种族或政治位置。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Nation-State (民族国家; en: nation-state)** imagines a people under common sovereignty; **Empire (帝国; en: empire)** governs heterogeneous populations through differentiated hierarchy. (民族国家想象共同主权下的人民；帝国通过差异化等级治理异质人口。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** empire shows that modern political order was never only a story of citizenship and rights. It was also a story of unequal subjecthood. (帝国显示现代政治秩序从不只是公民身份和权利的故事，也是非平等臣属身份的故事。)  
  
### 5. Colonial Discourse: The Problem of Speaking the Colonized into Being  
  
`Colonial Discourse (殖民话语; fr: discours colonial; en: colonial discourse)`  
**Definition:** the system of statements, images, classifications, narratives, and institutions through which colonial power represents, knows, governs, and produces the colonized. (殖民权力借以表象、认识、治理和生产被殖民者的一套陈述、图像、分类、叙事和制度系统。)  
**Problem solved:** it shows that colonialism rules not only through force, but also through representation and knowledge. (它显示殖民主义不只通过暴力统治，也通过表象和知识统治。)  
**Why needed:** the colonized are often made governable by being described as backward, childlike, irrational, tribal, feminine, violent, lazy, sensual, or incapable of self-rule. (被殖民者常通过被描述为落后、幼稚、非理性、部落化、女性化、暴力、懒惰、感性或不能自治而变得可治理。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing colonial archives, travel writing, missionary reports, school curricula, legal categories, ethnography, or imperial media. (当分析殖民档案、旅行写作、传教报告、学校课程、法律分类、民族志或帝国媒体时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Colonial discourse is not merely a set of lies. Its power is stronger. It produces categories that organize reality. It defines who is civilized, who is native, who is customary, who is modern, who is rational, who is dangerous, and who needs administration.  
  
This is where Foucault is indispensable. Colonial knowledge is **Power/Knowledge (权力/知识; fr: savoir-pouvoir; en: power/knowledge)**: it does not merely describe colonized reality; it reorganizes reality into governable forms.  
  
Concrete examples make this visible: maps turn complex local space into clear administrative regions; census categories fix fluid identities into groups; land registration converts customary and shared land relations into state-manageable property; surveys of customary law freeze dynamic local practice into texts usable by courts and administrators.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Colonial discourse produces the colonized as an object that can be known, represented, managed, improved, and ruled. (殖民话语把被殖民者生产为可以被认识、表象、管理、改良和统治的对象。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Description (描述; en: description)** seems neutral; **Colonial Discourse (殖民话语; en: colonial discourse)** describes in ways that classify, rank, and govern. (描述显得中立；殖民话语以分类、排序和治理的方式进行描述。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** colonial discourse links postcolonial theory to Foucault. Knowledge is not outside colonial power; it is one of its main instruments. (殖民话语把后殖民理论连接到福柯。知识不在殖民权力之外；它是殖民权力的主要工具之一。)  
  
### 6. Orientalism: The Problem of the West Producing the East  
  
`Orientalism (东方主义; fr: orientalisme; en: Orientalism)`  
**Definition:** Edward Said’s term for the Western discourse that constructs “the Orient” as exotic, backward, irrational, sensual, despotic, feminine, and in need of Western interpretation or rule. (爱德华·赛义德用来指西方话语如何把“东方”建构为异域的、落后的、非理性的、感性的、专制的、女性化的，并且需要西方解释或统治的对象。)  
**Problem solved:** it shows that “East” and “West” are not neutral geographical categories, but political-cultural constructions. (它显示“东方”和“西方”并非中立地理分类，而是政治—文化建构。)  
**Why needed:** the West confirms its own identity as rational, modern, free, active, masculine, and civilized by representing the East as its opposite. (西方通过把东方表象为自身反面，确认自身作为理性、现代、自由、主动、男性化和文明的身份。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing scholarship, literature, travel writing, media, foreign policy, colonial administration, art, or stereotypes about “the East.” (当分析学术、文学、旅行写作、媒体、外交政策、殖民行政、艺术或关于“东方”的刻板印象时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Orientalism is not simply a false image of Asia or the Middle East. It is a discourse with institutional power. It organizes what can be said, who can speak, who is studied, who is represented, and who is denied equal authority to interpret themselves.  
  
The key point is the structure exactly: Orientalism is not just the study of the East, but the way Western literature, scholarship, travel writing, art, colonial administration, and media construct “the East” as the opposite of the West. The East is described as mysterious, emotional, despotic, stagnant, feminized, backward, irrational, and needing interpretation and governance; the West appears as rational, modern, active, free, progressive, masculine, and civilized.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Orientalism makes the East into the West’s other so that the West can recognize itself as modern, rational, and superior. (东方主义把东方制造为西方的他者，使西方能够把自身认作现代、理性和优越。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Area Studies (区域研究; en: area studies)** can be a scholarly field; **Orientalism (东方主义; en: Orientalism)** names a power-laden discourse that constructs its object through hierarchy. (区域研究可以是学术领域；东方主义命名一种带有权力的等级化对象建构话语。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** Orientalism transforms representation into geopolitical power. To describe the East is also to position the West. (东方主义把表象转化为地缘政治权力。描述东方也就是定位西方。)  
  
### 7. Othering: The Problem of Identity through Exclusion  
  
`Othering (他者化; en: othering; fr: altérisation)`  
**Definition:** the process by which a group defines itself as normal, civilized, rational, or superior by producing another group as abnormal, primitive, irrational, or inferior. (一个群体通过把另一群体生产为异常、原始、非理性或低等者，来把自身定义为正常、文明、理性或优越的过程。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains identity formation through hierarchical exclusion. (它解释身份如何通过等级性排除形成。)  
**Why needed:** colonial identity often depends on constructing the colonized as the negative mirror of the colonizer. (殖民身份常依赖把被殖民者建构为殖民者的负面镜像。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing civilization/barbarism, modern/traditional, rational/irrational, developed/backward, white/nonwhite, West/East, human/savage. (当分析文明/野蛮、现代/传统、理性/非理性、发达/落后、白人/非白人、西方/东方、人/野蛮人时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Othering is not just difference. Difference can be horizontal. Othering is hierarchical. The other is made into the condition of the self’s superiority.  
  
This is why colonial discourse is full of binaries. The colonizer becomes rational because the colonized is irrational. The colonizer becomes modern because the colonized is traditional. The colonizer becomes masculine because the colonized is feminized. The colonizer becomes moral because the colonized is represented as corrupt, violent, sensual, or childlike.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Othering produces the colonized as a negative mirror through which the colonizer recognizes itself as superior. (他者化把被殖民者生产为负面镜像，殖民者借此把自身认作优越。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Difference (差异; fr: différence)** marks distinction; **Othering (他者化; en: othering)** organizes distinction into hierarchy and domination. (差异标记区别；他者化把区别组织成等级和支配。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** othering connects postcolonial theory with feminism, existentialism, psychoanalysis, and deconstruction. The Other is no longer only interpersonal; it is geopolitical and imperial. (他者化把后殖民理论同女性主义、存在主义、精神分析和解构连接起来。他者不再只是人际性的，也是地缘政治和帝国性的。)  
  
### 8. Race and Racialization: The Problem of Making Difference Governable  
  
`Race (种族; en: race)`  
**Definition:** not a pure biological essence, but a historically produced social classification that organizes power, hierarchy, identity, labor, space, violence, and life chances. (不是纯生物本质，而是一种历史生产出来的社会分类，它组织权力、等级、身份、劳动、空间、暴力和生命机会。)  
**Problem solved:** it rejects both biological essentialism and color-blind denial of racial power. (它拒绝生物本质主义，也拒绝无视种族权力的“色盲”否认。)  
**Why needed:** race has structured slavery, colonial rule, migration, citizenship, land ownership, policing, medicine, education, and labor. (种族结构化了奴隶制、殖民统治、迁移、公民身份、土地所有、警务、医学、教育和劳动。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing socially produced hierarchies attached to ancestry, phenotype, culture, religion, nationality, or origin. (当分析附着于血统、表型、文化、宗教、国籍或来源的社会生产等级时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
`Racialization (种族化; en: racialization)`  
**Definition:** the process by which bodies, groups, religions, languages, spaces, or practices are assigned racial meaning and placed within racial hierarchy. (身体、群体、宗教、语言、空间或实践被赋予种族意义并被放入种族等级中的过程。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains race as a process rather than a fixed essence. (它把种族解释为过程，而非固定本质。)  
**Why needed:** different groups become racialized differently across periods, empires, states, and institutions. (不同群体在不同时期、帝国、国家和制度中以不同方式被种族化。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing how a group becomes marked as dangerous, primitive, foreign, unassimilable, criminal, exotic, or biologically/culturally inferior. (当分析一个群体如何被标记为危险、原始、外来、不可同化、犯罪化、异域化或生物/文化上低等时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Race is not a pure biological fact but a social classification and power system. Race determines who may own land, vote, migrate, receive education, obtain work, and avoid police violence; racial inequality can continue through housing, schooling, policing, employment, and healthcare.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Racialization makes certain bodies and groups readable as governable, dangerous, inferior, foreign, or exploitable. (种族化使某些身体和群体被读取为可治理的、危险的、低等的、外来的或可剥削的。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Ethnicity (族群性; en: ethnicity)** usually concerns shared culture, language, descent, or identity; **Race (种族; en: race)** concerns historically produced hierarchies attached to bodies, ancestry, and power. (族群性通常关涉共享文化、语言、血统或身份；种族关涉附着于身体、血统和权力的历史生产等级。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** race links colonial classification to modern state power. It is not a residue of premodern prejudice; it is deeply modern. (种族把殖民分类同现代国家权力连接起来。它不是前现代偏见的残余，而是深刻现代的东西。)  
  
### 9. Colonial Knowledge: The Problem of Classification as Rule  
  
`Colonial Knowledge (殖民知识; en: colonial knowledge)`  
**Definition:** knowledge produced under colonial conditions that classifies colonized lands, peoples, customs, languages, bodies, and histories for purposes of rule, extraction, reform, or surveillance. (在殖民条件下生产的知识，它为了统治、榨取、改造或监视而分类被殖民土地、人民、习俗、语言、身体和历史。)  
**Problem solved:** it shows that colonial knowledge is not neutral description but part of administrative power. (它显示殖民知识不是中立描述，而是行政权力的一部分。)  
**Why needed:** colonial rule depends on maps, censuses, ethnographies, legal codifications, land surveys, medical categories, and educational systems. (殖民统治依赖地图、人口普查、民族志、法律编纂、土地调查、医学分类和教育系统。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing how knowledge makes a colonized world legible to power. (当分析知识如何使殖民世界对权力而言变得可读时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Colonial knowledge often presents itself as scientific, benevolent, documentary, or reformist. But its categories can reorganize the colonized society itself. It may fix fluid identities, harden boundaries, invent “traditions,” classify land, divide communities, codify flexible customs, and define who counts as tribe, caste, race, native, criminal, or minority.  
  
The problem of colonial knowledge is not that it is simply false; the problem is that it reorganizes reality according to needs of governance. Colonized societies are forced to understand themselves through colonial categories; some identities are strengthened, some boundaries fixed, and some traditions reinvented.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Colonial knowledge makes the colonized world legible by translating it into categories useful for rule. (殖民知识通过把被殖民世界翻译成对统治有用的分类，使其变得可读。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Knowledge (知识; el: ἐπιστήμη)** can aim at truth; **Colonial Knowledge (殖民知识; en: colonial knowledge)** produces truth-effects inside relations of domination. (知识可以以真理为目标；殖民知识在支配关系内部生产真理效果。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** colonial knowledge extends Foucault’s power/knowledge into imperial space. Classification is not after domination; it is one of domination’s conditions. (殖民知识把福柯的权力/知识扩展到帝国空间。分类不是支配之后的附加物，而是支配的条件之一。)  
  
### 10. Representation: The Problem of Speaking For  
  
`Representation (表象/代表; la: repraesentatio; en: representation)`  
**Definition:** the act or structure by which a group, place, person, or culture is depicted, spoken for, made visible, or politically represented. (一个群体、地方、个人或文化被描绘、被代言、被使之可见或被政治代表的行动或结构。)  
**Problem solved:** it reveals that depiction and political voice are not neutral. (它揭示描绘与政治发声并不中立。)  
**Why needed:** colonial subjects are often represented by those who govern, study, rescue, classify, or speak over them. (殖民主体常由统治、研究、拯救、分类或压过其声音的人来代表。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing who speaks, who is spoken about, who is spoken for, and who is denied authority to self-represent. (当分析谁在说话、谁被谈论、谁被代言，以及谁被剥夺自我表述权威时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Representation has two meanings: depiction and political speaking-for. Postcolonial theory uses both. A colonized person may be represented in novels, ethnographies, photographs, exhibitions, films, schoolbooks, census categories, and legal records. They may also be politically represented by colonial officials, native elites, missionaries, NGOs, experts, or nationalist leaders.  
  
The danger is substitution. Someone speaks for the colonized while making the colonized silent.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Representation becomes colonial when the represented are made visible only through the authority of those who speak for them. (当被表象者只有通过代言者的权威才变得可见时，表象就成为殖民性的。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Depiction (描绘; en: depiction)** shows an image or account; **Representation (代表/表象; en: representation)** also involves authority, mediation, and political substitution. (描绘给出图像或说明；代表/表象还涉及权威、中介和政治替代。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** representation links postcolonial theory with aesthetics, politics, law, anthropology, media, and epistemology. The question is not only accuracy, but authority. (表象把后殖民理论同美学、政治、法律、人类学、媒体和认识论连接起来。问题不只是准确性，也是权威。)  
  
### 11. Subaltern: The Problem of the Unheard  
  
`Subaltern (底层者/属下者; it: subalterno; en: subaltern)`  
**Definition:** a structurally subordinated subject or group whose speech is not recognized within dominant political, colonial, archival, or epistemic systems. (在主导政治、殖民、档案或认识系统中，其言说不被承认为有效言说的结构性从属主体或群体。)  
**Problem solved:** it names not merely the poor or oppressed, but those whose voice cannot enter dominant representation as voice. (它命名的不只是贫穷者或受压迫者，而是其声音无法作为声音进入主导表象系统的人。)  
**Why needed:** some subjects are not only exploited; they are rendered politically and epistemically inaudible. (有些主体不只是被剥削；他们在政治和认识上被变得不可听见。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing peasants, colonized women, indigenous groups, informal workers, caste-oppressed groups, or others whose speech is mediated, translated, erased, or overwritten. (当分析农民、被殖民女性、原住民群体、非正规劳动者、受种姓压迫群体，或其言说被中介、翻译、抹除或覆盖者时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
The subaltern is associated especially with **Gayatri Chakravorty Spivak** and Subaltern Studies. The key problem is not whether the subaltern makes sounds or has consciousness. The problem is whether dominant structures can hear that speech as authoritative, political, and self-representing.  
  
This is why Spivak’s question “Can the subaltern speak?” is not a simple empirical question. It is a question about mediation, archive, translation, gender, class, colonial representation, and epistemic violence.  
  
**Typical sentence:** The subaltern is not silent by nature; the subaltern is made unheard by the structures that translate, represent, or erase them. (底层者并非天生沉默；底层者是被翻译、代表或抹除他们的结构制造为不可听见者。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Oppressed Group (受压迫群体; en: oppressed group)** can still have recognized political voice; **Subaltern (底层者; en: subaltern)** marks a position where voice is structurally blocked or overwritten. (受压迫群体仍可能拥有被承认的政治声音；底层者标记声音被结构性阻塞或覆盖的位置。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** subalternity radicalizes representation critique. The issue is not simply to give voice, but to transform the conditions under which voice becomes audible. (底层性激进化表象批判。问题不只是“给予声音”，而是转化声音变得可听的条件。)  
  
### 12. Epistemic Violence: The Problem of Knowledge as Harm  
  
`Epistemic Violence (认识暴力; en: epistemic violence)`  
**Definition:** harm done through systems of knowledge that erase, misrepresent, classify, silence, or make unintelligible the lives and meanings of subordinated groups. (通过知识系统造成的伤害，这些系统抹除、误表象、分类、沉默化或使从属群体的生活与意义不可理解。)  
**Problem solved:** it expands violence beyond physical force to include the violence of knowing and naming. (它把暴力从物理强制扩展到认识和命名的暴力。)  
**Why needed:** colonial and imperial power often works by defining what counts as knowledge and whose knowledge is dismissed. (殖民和帝国权力常通过定义什么算作知识，以及谁的知识被驳回而运作。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing archives, legal categories, ethnography, translation, development policy, expert discourse, or erasure of indigenous knowledge. (当分析档案、法律分类、民族志、翻译、发展政策、专家话语或原住民知识抹除时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Epistemic violence does not mean every disagreement is violence. It names systematic injury through knowledge regimes. A colonized community may be classified as primitive, its law as custom, its religion as superstition, its land as empty, its language as dialect, its medicine as folklore, and its resistance as disorder.  
  
The harm lies in the fact that these classifications have effects. They authorize schooling, conversion, dispossession, development, policing, and reform.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Epistemic violence occurs when a knowledge system makes a people knowable only by erasing the terms through which they understand themselves. (当一个知识系统只有通过抹除一个群体理解自身的术语才能使其变得可知时，认识暴力就发生了。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Error (错误; en: error)** is a false claim; **Epistemic Violence (认识暴力; en: epistemic violence)** is a systematic injury built into knowledge production and recognition. (错误是虚假主张；认识暴力是内置于知识生产和承认中的系统性伤害。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** epistemology becomes decolonial. The question is not only whether knowledge is justified, but whether its conditions of justification erase other worlds. (认识论变得去殖民化。问题不只是知识是否被证成，也包括其证成条件是否抹除其他世界。)  
  
### 13. Voice: The Problem of Being Heard as a Subject  
  
`Voice (声音/发声; la: vox; en: voice)`  
**Definition:** not merely expression, but socially recognized capacity to speak, be heard, and affect interpretation or decision. (不仅是表达，也是被社会承认的说话、被听见并影响解释或决策的能力。)  
**Problem solved:** it distinguishes speaking from being recognized as a speaker. (它把说话同被承认为说话者区分开来。)  
**Why needed:** colonized and subaltern subjects may speak while dominant institutions hear only noise, testimony needing translation, emotion, folklore, threat, or ignorance. (被殖民和底层主体可能在说话，但主导制度只听见噪音、需要翻译的证词、情绪、民俗、威胁或无知。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing testimony, translation, law, media, activism, subalternity, indigenous claims, or archival absence. (当分析证词、翻译、法律、媒体、行动主义、底层性、原住民主张或档案缺席时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Voice is not guaranteed by speech. A courtroom, university, archive, development agency, or media system may allow someone to speak while stripping their speech of authority. Voice requires recognition, uptake, and consequences.  
  
This is why postcolonial theory distrusts easy calls to “let the oppressed speak.” The oppressed may already be speaking. The harder problem is whether dominant structures can hear without translating the speech back into imperial categories.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Voice is not the mere production of speech, but the social recognition of speech as meaningful and authoritative. (声音不是单纯发出话语，而是话语作为有意义和有权威之物被社会承认。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Speech (言说; en: speech)** is utterance; **Voice (声音; en: voice)** is socially recognized speech with standing. (言说是发话；声音是具有地位的被社会承认的言说。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** voice connects postcolonial theory with feminism, law, testimony, trauma studies, and democratic theory. Recognition becomes a condition of speech itself. (声音把后殖民理论同女性主义、法律、证词、创伤研究和民主理论连接起来。承认成为言说本身的条件。)  
  
### 14. Decolonization: The Problem of Liberation beyond Flag Independence  
  
`Decolonization (去殖民化; en: decolonization; fr: décolonisation)`  
**Definition:** the political, economic, cultural, epistemic, and psychic process of dismantling colonial rule and its continuing structures. (拆除殖民统治及其延续结构的政治、经济、文化、认识论和心理过程。)  
**Problem solved:** it prevents independence from being reduced to transfer of state power. (它防止独立被化约为国家权力移交。)  
**Why needed:** colonial power can persist after formal independence through language, borders, education, law, economy, race, knowledge, debt, and elite formation. (殖民权力可以在正式独立后通过语言、边界、教育、法律、经济、种族、知识、债务和精英形成继续存在。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing anti-colonial struggle, curriculum reform, land return, linguistic recovery, epistemic repair, economic sovereignty, or institutional transformation. (当分析反殖民斗争、课程改革、土地归还、语言复兴、认识修复、经济主权或制度转化时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Decolonization is not just replacing foreign rulers with national rulers. That may be necessary, but insufficient. A postcolonial state may inherit colonial borders, legal systems, police forms, education hierarchies, racial categories, export dependency, and elite languages.  
  
This is why decolonization has several layers: political independence, economic restructuring, cultural recovery, epistemic transformation, psychic disalienation, and institutional redesign.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Decolonization is incomplete when colonial categories, dependencies, and hierarchies survive inside formally independent institutions. (当殖民分类、依赖和等级继续存在于形式独立的制度内部时，去殖民化就是不完整的。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Independence (独立; en: independence)** can mean formal sovereignty; **Decolonization (去殖民化; en: decolonization)** means dismantling colonial structures across politics, economy, knowledge, culture, and subjectivity. (独立可以指形式主权；去殖民化意味着在政治、经济、知识、文化和主体性层面拆除殖民结构。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** liberation becomes structural and epistemic, not only national. Decolonization asks what remains colonial after colonial rule ends. (解放变得结构化和认识论化，而不只是民族化。去殖民化追问殖民统治结束后什么仍然是殖民性的。)  
  
### 15. Anti-Colonial Nationalism: The Problem of Freedom through Nation  
  
`Anti-Colonial Nationalism (反殖民民族主义; en: anti-colonial nationalism)`  
**Definition:** a political project that mobilizes national identity, peoplehood, sovereignty, and collective liberation against colonial rule. (一种政治工程，它动员民族身份、人民性、主权和集体解放来反抗殖民统治。)  
**Problem solved:** it gives colonized peoples a collective form for resisting empire and claiming self-rule. (它为被殖民人民提供反抗帝国并要求自治的集体形式。)  
**Why needed:** colonial power often denies colonized peoples political unity, historical agency, and sovereign capacity. (殖民权力常否认被殖民人民的政治统一、历史行动能力和主权能力。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing independence movements, national liberation, revolutionary culture, anti-imperial solidarity, or postcolonial state formation. (当分析独立运动、民族解放、革命文化、反帝团结或后殖民国家形成时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Anti-colonial nationalism is ambivalent. It can organize liberation. It can also reproduce exclusions: minority suppression, gender hierarchy, linguistic homogenization, state authoritarianism, or elite capture. Postcolonial theory therefore does not simply celebrate nationalism or dismiss it. It asks what kind of nation is being imagined, who belongs, who is excluded, and what colonial forms are inherited.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Anti-colonial nationalism can resist empire, but it can also inherit the state forms and exclusions through which empire governed. (反殖民民族主义能够反抗帝国，但也可能继承帝国用以治理的国家形式和排除机制。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **National Liberation (民族解放; en: national liberation)** aims to free a people from colonial rule; **Nationalism (民族主义; en: nationalism)** can also become a homogenizing or exclusionary state ideology. (民族解放旨在使人民摆脱殖民统治；民族主义也可能成为同质化或排他性国家意识形态。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** nation becomes both tool and problem. It is a weapon against empire, but not automatically a guarantee of decolonial justice. (民族成为工具也成为问题。它是反抗帝国的武器，但并不自动保证去殖民正义。)  
  
### 16. Fanon: The Problem of Colonial Violence and Psychic Alienation  
  
`Colonial Alienation (殖民异化; fr: aliénation coloniale)`  
**Definition:** the psychic and social splitting produced when colonized subjects are forced to see themselves through the colonizer’s racial, linguistic, and cultural categories. (当被殖民主体被迫通过殖民者的种族、语言和文化分类看待自身时产生的心理与社会分裂。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains colonial domination as bodily and psychic, not merely administrative. (它把殖民支配解释为身体和心理层面的，而不只是行政层面的。)  
**Why needed:** colonialism produces inferiority, shame, desire for recognition, internalized racism, and violent contradiction. (殖民主义生产自卑、羞耻、承认欲望、内化种族主义和暴力性矛盾。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing Frantz Fanon, racialized subjectivity, colonial language, bodily schema, violence, and liberation struggle. (当分析弗朗茨·法农、种族化主体性、殖民语言、身体图式、暴力和解放斗争时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
**Frantz Fanon** is indispensable because he joins psychoanalysis, phenomenology, Marxism, race, colonial violence, and anti-colonial revolution. Colonialism does not only exploit labor and land. It attacks the body-schema and self-relation of the colonized. The colonized subject is made visible through racial categories before being recognized as a person.  
  
Fanon also insists that decolonization is not polite reform. Colonial rule is founded in violence; anti-colonial struggle confronts that violence. This claim should be read carefully: Fanon is diagnosing colonial reality, not merely celebrating violence abstractly.  
  
**Algeria** and Fanon are key for understanding colonial violence, especially France’s long colonial rule and the second-class status imposed on local Muslim populations.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Fanon shows that colonialism enters the body and psyche by forcing the colonized to inhabit a racialized image produced by the colonizer. (法农显示殖民主义进入身体和心理，它迫使被殖民者居住在由殖民者生产的种族化形象中。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Exploitation (剥削; fr: exploitation)** concerns extraction of labor or value; **Colonial Alienation (殖民异化; fr: aliénation coloniale)** concerns the deformation of self-relation under racial-colonial power. (剥削关涉劳动或价值榨取；殖民异化关涉种族—殖民权力下自我关系的变形。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** Fanon makes postcolonial theory psycho-political. Liberation must address land, state, economy, body, language, and psychic life. (法农使后殖民理论成为心理—政治理论。解放必须处理土地、国家、经济、身体、语言和心理生活。)  
  
### 17. Mimicry: The Problem of Almost the Same  
  
`Mimicry (拟态/模仿; en: mimicry)`  
**Definition:** Homi Bhabha’s term for the colonized subject’s partial imitation of the colonizer’s language, manners, education, law, and culture, producing resemblance with difference. (霍米·巴巴用来指被殖民主体对殖民者语言、礼仪、教育、法律和文化的部分模仿，从而产生带有差异的相似性。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains colonial subject formation as ambivalent rather than simple assimilation. (它把殖民主体形成解释为暧昧的，而非简单同化。)  
**Why needed:** colonial power wants colonized intermediaries who are useful and similar, but not fully equal. (殖民权力需要有用且相似的本地中介者，但又不愿其完全平等。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing colonial education, native elites, bureaucratic intermediaries, accent, dress, legal language, missionary conversion, or cultural imitation. (当分析殖民教育、本地精英、官僚中介、口音、服饰、法律语言、传教改宗或文化模仿时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Mimicry is not passive copying. It is unstable. The colonized subject becomes “almost the same, but not quite.” That resemblance disturbs colonial authority. The colonizer wants imitation, but imitation can become mockery, excess, strategic appropriation, or anti-colonial reversal.  
  
Colonized subjects enter colonial schools, learn colonial language, law, science, administration, and manners, and may become lawyers, teachers, doctors, translators, and civil servants. But this mimicry is not complete obedience; Bhabha’s **Mimicry** and **Hybridity** show that colonial subjects are both like the colonizer and not fully like the colonizer.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Mimicry unsettles colonial authority because it produces a colonized subject who is almost the same as the colonizer, but never fully the same. (拟态动摇殖民权威，因为它生产出一个几乎像殖民者、但永远不完全相同的被殖民主体。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Assimilation (同化; en: assimilation)** suggests absorption into the dominant culture; **Mimicry (拟态; en: mimicry)** preserves a difference that makes imitation unstable and potentially subversive. (同化暗示被吸收到主导文化中；拟态保留差异，使模仿变得不稳定并可能具有颠覆性。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** mimicry changes the theory of colonial power. Power is strong, but it cannot fully control the meanings it forces colonized subjects to repeat. (拟态改变殖民权力理论。权力很强，但无法完全控制它迫使被殖民主体重复的意义。)  
  
### 18. Hybridity: The Problem of Mixed Colonial Culture  
  
`Hybridity (混杂性; en: hybridity)`  
**Definition:** the cultural, linguistic, political, and symbolic mixing produced by colonial encounter, translation, imitation, resistance, and appropriation. (殖民遭遇、翻译、模仿、抵抗和挪用所生产的文化、语言、政治和象征混合。)  
**Problem solved:** it rejects pure models of colonizer and colonized culture. (它拒绝殖民者文化与被殖民者文化的纯粹模型。)  
**Why needed:** colonial contact produces new forms that are neither simply Western nor simply indigenous. (殖民接触生产既非简单西方、也非简单本土的新形式。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing language mixing, legal translation, religious syncretism, nationalist discourse, colonial education, diaspora culture, or postcolonial literature. (当分析语言混合、法律翻译、宗教融合、民族主义话语、殖民教育、离散文化或后殖民文学时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Hybridity is not mere multicultural mixture. In Bhabha, it is a site of ambivalence. Colonial authority depends on translation and repetition, but translation changes what it repeats. The colonized may use the colonizer’s concepts—rights, law, equality, freedom, nation—against colonial rule itself.  
  
Colonized intellectuals can use European languages of liberty, equality, nation, rights, and rule of law against colonial domination; Indian nationalism, African anti-colonial movements, Caribbean anti-colonial literature, and Algerian revolutionary thought all contain this reverse use.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Hybridity names the unstable space where colonial meanings are repeated, altered, and turned against colonial authority. (混杂性命名殖民意义被重复、改变并反向作用于殖民权威的不稳定空间。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Purity (纯粹性; en: purity)** imagines culture as sealed and original; **Hybridity (混杂性; en: hybridity)** treats culture as formed through translation, encounter, and conflict. (纯粹性把文化想象为封闭且原初；混杂性把文化视为通过翻译、遭遇和冲突形成。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** hybridity gives postcolonial theory a non-binary model. Colonial culture is not simply domination versus authenticity; it is also appropriation, mixture, distortion, and counter-use. (混杂性为后殖民理论提供非二元模型。殖民文化不只是支配与真实性的对立，也是挪用、混合、扭曲和反向使用。)  
  
### 19. Ambivalence: The Problem of Unstable Colonial Authority  
  
`Ambivalence (暧昧性/两价性; en: ambivalence)`  
**Definition:** the instability of colonial authority, which desires similarity and difference, reform and hierarchy, assimilation and exclusion at the same time. (殖民权威的不稳定性：它同时欲望相似与差异、改造与等级、同化与排除。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains why colonial discourse is anxious, repetitive, and contradictory. (它解释为什么殖民话语焦虑、重复且矛盾。)  
**Why needed:** colonial power must make the colonized governable and educable, but also keep them inferior. (殖民权力必须使被殖民者可治理、可教育，却又必须使其保持低等位置。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing contradictions in colonial education, civilizing mission, native elite formation, missionary reform, or liberal imperialism. (当分析殖民教育、文明使命、本地精英形成、传教改革或自由帝国主义中的矛盾时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Ambivalence is the structure behind mimicry. The colonizer wants the colonized to learn the colonizer’s language, but fears equality. The colonizer wants law and order, but denies equal legal standing. The colonizer wants civilization, but preserves racial hierarchy. The colonizer wants local intermediaries, but distrusts their authority.  
  
This contradiction does not merely weaken empire. It also produces openings for resistance.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Colonial authority is ambivalent because it needs the colonized to become similar enough to govern, but different enough to subordinate. (殖民权威是暧昧的，因为它需要被殖民者变得足够相似以便治理，又必须保持足够不同以便从属。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Contradiction (矛盾; de: Widerspruch)** can be logical or structural opposition; **Ambivalence (暧昧性; en: ambivalence)** names a conflicted desire within colonial authority itself. (矛盾可以是逻辑或结构对立；暧昧性命名殖民权威自身内部的冲突性欲望。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** ambivalence prevents simple models of domination. Empire is violent and powerful, but also anxious and unstable. (暧昧性防止支配模型过于简单。帝国是暴力且强大的，但也是焦虑且不稳定的。)  
  
### 20. Diaspora: The Problem of Displaced Belonging  
  
`Diaspora (离散; el: διασπορά; en: diaspora)`  
**Definition:** the dispersion of a people across regions or nations, producing forms of belonging shaped by migration, memory, displacement, racialization, and transnational relation. (一个人民跨区域或国家的分散，由迁移、记忆、位移、种族化和跨国关系塑造归属形式。)  
**Problem solved:** it challenges nation-centered models of identity and culture. (它挑战以民族国家为中心的身份与文化模型。)  
**Why needed:** colonialism, slavery, indenture, war, partition, labor migration, exile, and globalization produce identities that do not fit one homeland/one nation models. (殖民主义、奴隶制、契约劳工、战争、分裂、劳工迁移、流亡和全球化生产不符合一个故乡/一个民族模型的身份。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing migration, exile, memory, transnational identity, racialized belonging, language loss, or cultural transmission. (当分析迁移、流亡、记忆、跨国身份、种族化归属、语言丧失或文化传递时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Diaspora is not simply living abroad. It names a structured condition of belonging across distance. Diasporic subjects may belong to several places and to none completely. They carry memory, language, trauma, family networks, religious practices, food, music, racial classification, and political attachments across borders.  
  
Diaspora complicates nationalism. It also complicates assimilation. The diasporic subject may be told to integrate into the host nation while also being marked as foreign.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Diaspora names belonging that is stretched across displacement, memory, race, and transnational connection. (离散命名一种被位移、记忆、种族和跨国联系拉伸的归属。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Migration (迁移; la: migratio)** is movement across space; **Diaspora (离散; el: διασπορά)** is a historical and cultural formation of dispersed belonging. (迁移是跨空间移动；离散是分散归属的历史和文化构型。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** identity becomes transnational. Postcolonial theory moves beyond the colony/metropole binary toward routes, networks, memory, and circulation. (身份变得跨国化。后殖民理论超出殖民地/宗主国二元，转向路线、网络、记忆和流通。)  
  
### 21. Creolization: The Problem of New Worlds from Contact  
  
`Creolization (克里奥尔化; fr: créolisation; en: creolization)`  
**Definition:** the formation of new languages, cultures, identities, and social forms through colonial contact, slavery, migration, mixture, and survival. (通过殖民接触、奴隶制、迁移、混合和生存而形成新语言、文化、身份和社会形式的过程。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains cultural formation as creative mixture under unequal historical conditions. (它把文化形成解释为不平等历史条件下的创造性混合。)  
**Why needed:** colonial worlds did not merely preserve old identities or impose European forms; they produced new forms. (殖民世界不只是保留旧身份或强加欧洲形式；它们生产了新形式。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing Caribbean culture, language formation, music, religion, food, literature, racial mixture, or plantation societies. (当分析加勒比文化、语言形成、音乐、宗教、食物、文学、种族混合或种植园社会时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Creolization is related to hybridity, but often more grounded in the histories of slavery, plantation, forced migration, and language formation. It stresses creativity under domination. New forms emerge not because power is benign, but because survival requires invention.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Creolization names the creation of new cultural forms under conditions of displacement, violence, and unequal contact. (克里奥尔化命名在位移、暴力和不平等接触条件下新文化形式的创造。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Hybridity (混杂性; en: hybridity)** is a broad concept of mixed cultural formation; **Creolization (克里奥尔化; en: creolization)** often emphasizes colonial contact zones, slavery, language, and plantation history. (混杂性是关于混合文化形成的广义概念；克里奥尔化常强调殖民接触区、奴隶制、语言和种植园历史。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** creolization turns cultural loss into a more complex story: domination destroys, but dominated peoples also create new worlds. (克里奥尔化把文化丧失转化为更复杂的故事：支配会摧毁，但被支配者也会创造新世界。)  
  
### 22. Settler Colonialism: The Problem of Replacement  
  
`Settler Colonialism (定居殖民主义; en: settler colonialism)`  
**Definition:** a colonial form in which settlers seek not only to rule indigenous peoples, but to replace them and claim permanent sovereignty over land. (一种殖民形式，定居者不仅试图统治原住民，而且试图取代他们，并对土地宣称永久主权。)  
**Problem solved:** it distinguishes settlement and elimination from extraction-only models of colonialism. (它把定居与消除逻辑同单纯榨取模型区分开来。)  
**Why needed:** settler colonialism centers land, elimination, property, sovereignty, indigenous erasure, and replacement. (定居殖民主义以土地、消除、财产、主权、原住民抹除和取代为中心。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing indigenous dispossession, frontier myths, land law, reservations, assimilation schools, sovereignty conflicts, or elimination narratives. (当分析原住民被剥夺、边疆神话、土地法、保留地、同化学校、主权冲突或消除叙事时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Settler colonialism is not an event that ends when conquest ends. It is a structure that continues through land title, state sovereignty, property law, education, policing, environmental extraction, and narratives of national origin.  
  
Its logic is not merely “exploit the native.” It often seeks to make the native disappear as sovereign presence: physically, legally, culturally, demographically, or narratively.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Settler colonialism seeks to make the settler appear native to the land by erasing indigenous sovereignty. (定居殖民主义通过抹除原住民主权，使定居者显得像土地的原生者。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Extractive Colonialism (榨取型殖民主义; en: extractive colonialism)** primarily seeks labor and resources; **Settler Colonialism (定居殖民主义; en: settler colonialism)** seeks land and replacement. (榨取型殖民主义主要追求劳动和资源；定居殖民主义追求土地和取代。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** land becomes central. Postcolonial critique must address sovereignty, property, ecology, indigenous law, and ongoing occupation. (土地成为核心。后殖民批判必须处理主权、财产、生态、原住民法律和持续占领。)  
  
### 23. Neocolonialism: The Problem of Colonial Continuity after Independence  
  
`Neocolonialism (新殖民主义; en: neocolonialism)`  
**Definition:** the continuation of colonial-style dependency and domination after formal political independence through economic, military, cultural, technological, financial, or institutional means. (在正式政治独立之后，通过经济、军事、文化、技术、金融或制度手段延续殖民式依赖和支配。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains why formal sovereignty may coexist with dependency. (它解释为什么形式主权可以同依赖共存。)  
**Why needed:** postcolonial states may remain locked into unequal trade, debt, resource extraction, military alliances, language hierarchies, or expert-led development regimes. (后殖民国家可能仍被锁入不平等贸易、债务、资源榨取、军事联盟、语言等级或专家主导的发展体制。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing debt regimes, multinational corporations, aid dependency, military intervention, extractive economies, or development policy. (当分析债务体制、跨国公司、援助依赖、军事干预、榨取经济或发展政策时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Neocolonialism is why “postcolonial” does not simply mean “after colonialism.” It often means after formal colonial rule, but within continuing global hierarchy. Postcolonial theory therefore studies both past empire and present dependency.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Neocolonialism names the survival of colonial power inside formally independent global arrangements. (新殖民主义命名殖民权力在形式独立的全球配置中的延续。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Postcolonial (后殖民; en: postcolonial)** can name the condition after formal colonial rule; **Neocolonial (新殖民; en: neocolonial)** names the continuation of domination after that formal end. (后殖民可以命名正式殖民统治之后的状态；新殖民命名这种形式终结之后支配的继续。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** colonial critique becomes global political economy. The colony is no longer the only site of coloniality. (殖民批判转向全球政治经济。殖民地不再是殖民性的唯一场所。)  
  
### 24. World-System: The Problem of Core and Periphery  
  
`World-System (世界体系; en: world-system)`  
**Definition:** Immanuel Wallerstein’s model of capitalism as a global system structured by core, semi-periphery, and periphery rather than by isolated national economies. (伊曼纽尔·沃勒斯坦把资本主义理解为由核心、半边缘和边缘结构化的全球体系，而非孤立民族经济的模型。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains global inequality as systemic position, not national failure alone. (它把全球不平等解释为体系位置问题，而不只是国家失败。)  
**Why needed:** capitalism operates through unequal exchange, global division of labor, extraction, finance, technology, military power, and dependent development. (资本主义通过不平等交换、全球劳动分工、榨取、金融、技术、军事权力和依附性发展运作。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing global capitalism, dependency, development, commodity chains, industrialization, resource extraction, or core/periphery relations. (当分析全球资本主义、依赖、发展、商品链、工业化、资源榨取或核心/边缘关系时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
World-systems theory treats capitalism as a global system, with core regions controlling high-profit industries, finance, technology, and military power; peripheral regions providing raw materials, cheap labor, and low-profit production; and semi-peripheral regions occupying intermediate positions.  
  
This matters because the language of “advanced” and “backward” often hides structural relation. Peripheral regions are not simply behind on the same road. They may be kept peripheral by the way the world-system organizes value, labor, debt, technology, and trade.  
  
**Typical sentence:** World-systems theory turns development from a national ladder into a global relation of unequal positions. (世界体系理论把发展从民族国家阶梯转化为不平等位置的全球关系。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Modernization Theory (现代化理论; en: modernization theory)** often imagines all societies moving through similar stages; **World-System Theory (世界体系理论; en: world-system theory)** analyzes unequal positions within one global capitalist system. (现代化理论常想象所有社会经过相似阶段；世界体系理论分析同一全球资本主义体系内部的不平等位置。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** postcolonial critique meets political economy. Empire is not only representation; it is also value transfer, labor hierarchy, and global accumulation. (后殖民批判同政治经济学汇合。帝国不只是表象，也是价值转移、劳动等级和全球积累。)  
  
### 25. Decoloniality: The Problem of Coloniality after Colonialism  
  
`Decoloniality (去殖民性; en: decoloniality; es: decolonialidad)`  
**Definition:** a theoretical and political project that analyzes and contests the ongoing coloniality of power, knowledge, being, gender, race, and economy after formal colonial rule. (一种理论与政治工程，它分析并反抗正式殖民统治之后仍持续存在的权力、知识、存在、性别、种族和经济的殖民性。)  
**Problem solved:** it distinguishes the end of colonial administration from the persistence of colonial structures in modernity itself. (它把殖民行政的终结同现代性自身中殖民结构的持续区分开来。)  
**Why needed:** coloniality can survive in epistemology, development, race, gender, religion, aesthetics, law, and global capitalism. (殖民性可以在认识论、发展、种族、性别、宗教、美学、法律和全球资本主义中继续存在。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing knowledge hierarchies, Eurocentrism, indigenous epistemologies, racial capitalism, colonial gender systems, or pluriversal politics. (当分析知识等级、欧洲中心主义、原住民认识论、种族资本主义、殖民性别系统或多元世界政治时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Decoloniality is related to postcolonial theory but often more explicitly criticizes the coloniality of modernity itself. It asks not only how empire represented others, but how the modern world-order still ranks knowledge, humanity, spirituality, economy, and being according to colonial lines.  
  
A decolonial approach often asks for **pluriversality**: not one universal model imposed everywhere, but many worlds, epistemologies, legalities, and life-forms in relation.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Decoloniality asks what remains colonial in modern reason, knowledge, economy, and being even after formal empire ends. (去殖民性追问即使正式帝国终结之后，现代性理性、知识、经济和存在中仍有什么是殖民性的。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Postcolonial Theory (后殖民理论; en: postcolonial theory)** often emerged through literary theory, discourse analysis, and critique of representation; **Decoloniality (去殖民性; es: decolonialidad)** often emphasizes coloniality as constitutive of modernity and calls for epistemic delinking. (后殖民理论常通过文学理论、话语分析和表象批判形成；去殖民性常强调殖民性构成现代性，并要求认识论脱钩。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** critique moves from empire as historical event to coloniality as ongoing structure of modern world-making. (批判从作为历史事件的帝国转向作为现代世界建构持续结构的殖民性。)  
  
### 26. The Postcolonial Diagnostic Method  
  
Postcolonial analysis should not become a generic accusation that everything Western is false. That is too weak. The method is more precise.  
  
A strong postcolonial reading asks:  
  
**What colonial or imperial relation makes this concept possible?**  
(什么殖民或帝国关系使这个概念成为可能？)  
  
**Who is represented, and who has authority to represent?**  
(谁被表象？谁拥有表象权威？)  
  
**What binary organizes the field: West/East, modern/backward, civilized/barbaric, rational/irrational, developed/underdeveloped?**  
(什么二元对立组织了这一场域：西方/东方、现代/落后、文明/野蛮、理性/非理性、发达/欠发达？)  
  
**What knowledge practice makes the colonized world governable: map, census, archive, law, school, museum, ethnography, development index?**  
(什么知识实践使被殖民世界变得可治理：地图、人口普查、档案、法律、学校、博物馆、民族志、发展指数？)  
  
**Whose voice is translated, mediated, or erased?**  
(谁的声音被翻译、中介或抹除？)  
  
**What remains colonial after formal colonialism ends?**  
(正式殖民主义结束之后，什么仍然是殖民性的？)  
  
**Typical sentence:** Postcolonial reading asks how empire makes a world knowable, governable, racialized, and narratable. (后殖民阅读追问帝国如何使一个世界变得可知、可治理、被种族化并可被叙述。)  
  
### 27. The Tool-Map of Postcolonial Theory  
  
Use postcolonial vocabulary diagnostically. The core question is usually not only “is this representation accurate?” but “what imperial relation gives this representation authority?”  
  
**If the text analyzes direct rule, extraction, settlement, or administration**, look for **Colonialism (殖民主义; en: colonialism)**, **Empire (帝国; en: empire)**, and **Colonial Discourse (殖民话语; en: colonial discourse)**.  
(如果文本分析直接统治、榨取、定居或行政，应寻找殖民主义、帝国和殖民话语问题。)  
  
**If the text analyzes domination beyond formal colonies**, look for **Imperialism (帝国主义; en: imperialism)** and **Neocolonialism (新殖民主义; en: neocolonialism)**.  
(如果文本分析超出正式殖民地的支配，应寻找帝国主义和新殖民主义问题。)  
  
**If the text analyzes West/East representations**, look for **Orientalism (东方主义; en: Orientalism)** and **Othering (他者化; en: othering)**.  
(如果文本分析西方/东方表象，应寻找东方主义和他者化问题。)  
  
**If the text analyzes race as a social power system**, look for **Race (种族; en: race)** and **Racialization (种族化; en: racialization)**.  
(如果文本把种族作为社会权力系统来分析，应寻找种族和种族化问题。)  
  
**If the text analyzes maps, censuses, law, ethnography, schools, archives, or museums**, look for **Colonial Knowledge (殖民知识; en: colonial knowledge)** and **Epistemic Violence (认识暴力; en: epistemic violence)**.  
(如果文本分析地图、人口普查、法律、民族志、学校、档案或博物馆，应寻找殖民知识和认识暴力问题。)  
  
**If the text asks who can speak or be heard**, look for **Subaltern (底层者; en: subaltern)**, **Voice (声音; en: voice)**, and **Representation (表象/代表; en: representation)**.  
(如果文本追问谁能说话或被听见，应寻找底层者、声音和表象/代表问题。)  
  
**If the text analyzes anti-colonial struggle**, look for **Decolonization (去殖民化; en: decolonization)**, **Anti-Colonial Nationalism (反殖民民族主义; en: anti-colonial nationalism)**, and **Fanonian Colonial Alienation (法农式殖民异化; fr: aliénation coloniale)**.  
(如果文本分析反殖民斗争，应寻找去殖民化、反殖民民族主义和法农式殖民异化问题。)
