**If the text analyzes colonial imitation and unstable identity**, look for **Mimicry (拟态; en: mimicry)**, **Hybridity (混杂性; en: hybridity)**, and **Ambivalence (暧昧性; en: ambivalence)**.  
(如果文本分析殖民模仿和不稳定身份，应寻找拟态、混杂性和暧昧性问题。)  
  
**If the text analyzes migration and displaced belonging**, look for **Diaspora (离散; en: diaspora)** and **Creolization (克里奥尔化; en: creolization)**.  
(如果文本分析迁移和位移归属，应寻找离散和克里奥尔化问题。)  
  
**If the text analyzes indigenous land and replacement**, look for **Settler Colonialism (定居殖民主义; en: settler colonialism)** and **Indigeneity (原住民性; en: indigeneity)**.  
(如果文本分析原住民土地和取代，应寻找定居殖民主义和原住民性问题。)  
  
**If the text analyzes global capitalism**, look for **World-System (世界体系; en: world-system)**, **Core/Periphery (核心/边缘; en: core/periphery)**, and **Dependency (依附; en: dependency)**.  
(如果文本分析全球资本主义，应寻找世界体系、核心/边缘和依附问题。)  
  
**If the text asks what remains colonial inside modernity itself**, look for **Decoloniality (去殖民性; es: decolonialidad)** and **Coloniality (殖民性; es: colonialidad)**.  
(如果文本追问现代性自身内部什么仍是殖民性的，应寻找去殖民性和殖民性问题。)  
  
### 28. The Genealogical Point of Part 17  
  
Postcolonial theory transforms the philosophical language of modernity. Earlier philosophy often narrated modernity through **reason**, **science**, **freedom**, **rights**, **capital**, **subjectivity**, and **progress**. Feminism showed that this subject was gendered and dependent on hidden labor. Foucault showed that knowledge and power produce subjects and truth. Derrida showed that conceptual hierarchies depend on excluded terms. Psychoanalysis showed that the subject is split by desire and the Other.  
  
Postcolonial theory adds:  
  
**Modernity was imperial, racialized, extractive, and epistemically violent.**  
(现代性是帝国性的、种族化的、榨取性的和认识暴力性的。)  
  
The guiding thesis is:  
  
**Postcolonial language turns philosophy toward empire’s hidden conditions: to understand a concept, institution, archive, nation, race, or representation is to ask what colonial relation produced it, what hierarchy it naturalizes, whose voice it silences, what knowledge makes it governable, and what global structure continues to profit from it.**  
(后殖民语言把哲学转向帝国的隐藏条件：理解一个概念、制度、档案、民族、种族或表象，就是追问什么殖民关系生产了它，它自然化了什么等级，沉默化了谁的声音，什么知识使它变得可治理，以及什么全球结构仍然从中获利。)  
  
This grammar prepares the next stage: **Pragmatism and Ordinary Language Philosophy**. After postcolonial theory exposes the imperial history of universal concepts, pragmatism and ordinary language philosophy will ask how concepts function in practice, how meanings live in use, and how philosophy can return from abstraction to forms of life.  
  
The postcolonial question remains one of the strongest tools for philosophical reading:  
  
**What empire, archive, racial order, or global hierarchy must be forgotten for this concept to appear universal, civilized, and progressive?**  
(为了使这个概念显得普遍、文明且进步，什么帝国、档案、种族秩序或全球等级必须被遗忘？)  
  
## Part 18. Pragmatism and Ordinary Language Philosophy: Practice, Use, Form of Life  
  
This chapter explains **Pragmatism** and **Ordinary Language Philosophy** as two traditions that return philosophy from abstract foundations to **practice**, **use**, **habit**, **inquiry**, **language-games**, and **forms of life**. After postcolonial theory, the danger is that philosophical critique may remain at the level of large structures: empire, archive, discourse, race, capital, gender, power. Pragmatism and ordinary language philosophy add another discipline: **ask how a concept actually works in practice, in inquiry, in ordinary use, and in shared forms of life**. (追问一个概念实际上如何在实践、探究、日常使用和共享生活形式中运作。)  
  
The central vocabulary is **Pragmatism**, **Practice**, **Consequence**, **Inquiry**, **Habit**, **Fallibilism**, **Abduction**, **Belief**, **Doubt**, **Truth**, **Experience**, **Use**, **Meaning as Use**, **Language-Game**, **Form of Life**, **Rule-Following**, **Family Resemblance**, **Ordinary Language**, **Speech Act**, **Performative**, **Category Mistake**, and **Therapy**.  
  
**Pragmatism** is an American philosophical tradition represented by **Charles Sanders Peirce**, **William James**, and **John Dewey**. It is not the vulgar thesis “whatever is useful is true,” but a way of understanding meaning, truth, and value through **practice**, **consequences**, **inquiry**, and **problem-solving**. Pragmatism also connects with **abduction**: pragmatic reasoning does not assume that truth about independent reality can be irrefutably established; it asks how inquiry can make the best available judgment under limited evidence and practical demands.  
  
The operational function of this chapter is exact: use pragmatist and ordinary-language vocabulary when the problem is **how a concept, belief, rule, word, or theory functions in actual practice, inquiry, language-use, and life**. (当问题是一个概念、信念、规则、词语或理论如何在实际实践、探究、语言使用和生活中发挥功能时，应使用实用主义与日常语言哲学词汇。)  
  
### 1. The Problem-Situation: Philosophy Must Return to Use  
  
Earlier traditions often asked for foundations. Metaphysics asked what is ultimately real. Epistemology asked what makes knowledge certain. Analytic philosophy asked what conditions define a concept. Structuralism asked what system makes meaning possible. Foucault asked what discourse makes statements authoritative. Derrida asked what hierarchy makes meaning appear stable.  
  
Pragmatism and ordinary language philosophy ask a more practical question:  
  
**What difference does this concept make in use?**  
(这个概念在使用中造成什么差异？)  
  
This question is not anti-theoretical. It is anti-idle. A concept should be tested by its role in inquiry, action, clarification, social coordination, and problem-solving. A word should be understood by how it is used in practices. A belief should be examined by the habits of action it supports. A philosophical problem should be checked against ordinary language, not because ordinary language is always correct, but because it often contains distinctions that abstract theory erases.  
  
The shared problem is:  
  
**When philosophy detaches meaning from practice, it produces pseudo-problems.**  
(当哲学把意义从实践中抽离时，它会制造伪问题。)  
  
**Typical sentence:** Pragmatism and ordinary language philosophy ask philosophy to test concepts by their practical consequences and ordinary uses. (实用主义与日常语言哲学要求哲学通过实践后果和日常使用来检验概念。)  
  
### 2. Pragmatism: The Problem of Meaning through Consequences  
  
`Pragmatism (实用主义; en: pragmatism)`  
**Definition:** a philosophical tradition that understands meaning, belief, truth, and value through practical consequences, inquiry, habit, and problem-solving. (一种哲学传统，它通过实践后果、探究、习惯和问题解决来理解意义、信念、真理和价值。)  
**Problem solved:** it prevents philosophy from treating concepts as detached abstractions with no practical difference. (它防止哲学把概念视为没有实践差异的抽象物。)  
**Why needed:** many disputes become clearer when one asks what would change in experience, action, inquiry, or conduct if a claim were accepted. (如果追问接受某个主张会在经验、行动、探究或行为中改变什么，许多争论会变得更清楚。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing what a belief, theory, or concept does in practice. (当分析一个信念、理论或概念在实践中做什么时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Pragmatism is often misunderstood as crude usefulness. That is too shallow. It does not say that any convenient belief is true. It says that meaning and truth must be understood within practices of inquiry and action. A concept without possible practical difference is empty or at least philosophically suspicious.  
  
For **Peirce**, the meaning of a concept lies in the conceivable practical effects connected with it. For **James**, truth is connected to what proves itself good in the way of belief under lived conditions. For **Dewey**, inquiry is a social and experimental process for transforming problematic situations.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Pragmatism asks what practical difference a belief or concept makes in inquiry and conduct. (实用主义追问一个信念或概念在探究和行为中造成什么实践差异。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Utility (效用; la: utilitas)** can mean immediate usefulness; **Pragmatism (实用主义; en: pragmatism)** analyzes meaning and truth through consequences within disciplined inquiry. (效用可以指直接有用性；实用主义则通过有规训的探究中的后果来分析意义与真理。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** pragmatism changes the question from “what is the timeless essence of this concept?” to “how does this concept guide action, inquiry, and adjustment to the world?” (实用主义把问题从“这个概念的永恒本质是什么？”转向“这个概念如何引导行动、探究和对世界的调适？”)  
  
### 3. Practice: The Problem of Concepts in Action  
  
`Practice (实践; el: πρᾶξις; en: practice)`  
**Definition:** organized human activity governed by habits, norms, purposes, tools, skills, and social contexts. (由习惯、规范、目的、工具、技能和社会语境支配的有组织人类活动。)  
**Problem solved:** it shows that concepts live in activities, not only in definitions. (它显示概念存在于活动中，而不只存在于定义中。)  
**Why needed:** many concepts cannot be understood apart from what people do with them. (许多概念不能脱离人们用它们做什么而被理解。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing law, science, education, medicine, politics, language, morality, or everyday life as structured activity. (当把法律、科学、教育、医学、政治、语言、道德或日常生活分析为结构化活动时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
**Transfer rule:** use **Practice** when meaning, knowledge, subjectivity, or social order must be understood through organized doing; do not use it merely as a synonym for “application” after theory. (转用规则：当意义、知识、主体性或社会秩序必须通过有组织的行动来理解时，才使用 Practice；不要把它仅仅当成理论之后的“应用”。)  
  
Practice is the point where thought becomes worldly. A legal concept works in courts, contracts, police practices, procedures, and judgments. A scientific concept works in experiments, instruments, measurement, prediction, and revision. A moral concept works in blame, praise, apology, repair, expectation, and responsibility.  
  
This is why purely verbal analysis can fail. A concept’s meaning may be distributed across institutions, habits, bodily training, expectations, and material tools.  
  
**Typical sentence:** To understand a concept pragmatically is to understand the practice in which it has work to do. (以实用主义方式理解一个概念，就是理解它在其中发挥作用的实践。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Theory (理论; el: θεωρία)** seeks articulation or explanation; **Practice (实践; el: πρᾶξις)** is organized doing. Pragmatism refuses to isolate theory from practice. (理论寻求阐明或解释；实践是有组织的行动。实用主义拒绝把理论从实践中孤立出来。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** practice becomes epistemic. Knowing is not only contemplation; it is intervention, testing, correction, and adjustment. (实践变成认识论问题。认识不只是沉思，也是介入、测试、修正和调适。)  
  
### 4. Consequence: The Problem of Practical Difference  
  
`Consequence (后果; la: consequentia; en: consequence)`  
**Definition:** the practical, experiential, inferential, or behavioral effect that follows from accepting, applying, or acting on a concept or belief. (接受、应用或按照一个概念或信念行动所产生的实践、经验、推论或行为效果。)  
**Problem solved:** it tests whether a philosophical distinction makes a real difference. (它检验一个哲学区分是否造成真实差异。)  
**Why needed:** some metaphysical disputes appear deep but generate no difference in inquiry or action. (有些形而上学争论显得深刻，却在探究或行动中不产生差异。)  
**How to use:** use it when asking what would change if a claim were true, false, accepted, or rejected. (当追问如果一个主张为真、为假、被接受或被拒绝，会改变什么时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
The pragmatist test is sharp: if two theories make no conceivable difference to experience, inquiry, prediction, action, or practice, the dispute may be verbal or empty. This does not eliminate metaphysics. It disciplines metaphysics.  
  
For example, a debate about whether “matter” is substance or bundle becomes pragmatically meaningful only if it changes explanation, prediction, ontology, scientific practice, or conceptual clarity. Otherwise, it may be a dispute over words.  
  
**Typical sentence:** A pragmatist asks what consequences a concept has for action, inquiry, and experience. (实用主义者追问一个概念对行动、探究和经验有什么后果。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Implication (暗示/含义; en: implication)** can be semantic or contextual; **Consequence (后果; en: consequence)** in pragmatism means practical effect in inquiry or conduct. (Implication 可以是语义或语境含义；实用主义中的 consequence 指探究或行为中的实践效果。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** meaning becomes operational. A concept’s reality is tested by the difference it makes. (意义变得操作化。一个概念的实在性由其造成的差异来检验。)  
  
### 5. Inquiry: The Problem of Thinking as Problem-Solving  
  
`Inquiry (探究; en: inquiry)`  
**Definition:** the disciplined process of transforming an uncertain or problematic situation into a more settled, intelligible, and workable one. (把不确定或成问题的处境转化为更稳定、可理解且可操作处境的有规训过程。)  
**Problem solved:** it treats knowledge as an activity rather than a static possession. (它把知识理解为活动，而非静态占有物。)  
**Why needed:** thinking begins when habitual action is disrupted and a situation becomes problematic. (当习惯性行动被打断，处境变得成问题时，思考开始。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing science, education, democratic deliberation, law, diagnosis, design, or moral problem-solving. (当分析科学、教育、民主审议、法律、诊断、设计或道德问题解决时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
For Dewey, inquiry begins in trouble. Something does not work. Expectation fails. Conflict appears. The task of thought is not to mirror reality from afar, but to reconstruct the situation so action can continue intelligently.  
  
This makes inquiry experimental. Hypotheses are tools. Concepts are instruments. Truth is not static possession but something won through tested inquiry.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Inquiry begins when a situation becomes problematic and ends provisionally when action can proceed intelligently. (探究始于处境变得成问题之时，并在行动能够明智继续时暂时结束。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Contemplation (沉思; la: contemplatio)** observes from distance; **Inquiry (探究; en: inquiry)** intervenes in a problematic situation. (沉思从距离中观察；探究介入成问题的处境。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** knowledge becomes experimental and social. It is not merely the mind’s possession of truth, but a communal method for coping with problems. (知识变得实验化和社会化。它不只是心灵对真理的占有，而是共同体应对问题的方法。)  
  
### 6. Habit: The Problem of Conduct before Reflection  
  
`Habit (习惯; la: habitus; en: habit)`  
**Definition:** a stabilized pattern of perception, action, response, and expectation that guides conduct before explicit reflection. (一种稳定的知觉、行动、反应和期待模式，它在明确反思之前引导行为。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains how intelligence operates through learned patterns, not only through conscious deliberation. (它解释智能如何通过习得模式运作，而不只是通过自觉思考运作。)  
**Why needed:** most conduct is not produced by isolated rational decisions; it is carried by habits. (大多数行为不是由孤立理性决策产生，而是由习惯承载。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing moral character, social practice, education, skill, prejudice, institutional routine, or embodied knowledge. (当分析道德品格、社会实践、教育、技能、偏见、制度惯例或具身知识时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Pragmatism treats habit as intelligent. A habit is not merely mechanical repetition. It is a way of being ready to act. Habits can be enabling or oppressive. They can allow skill, attention, and coordination; they can also reproduce prejudice, domination, and unthinking conformity.  
  
This links pragmatism to later social theory. Race, gender, class, law, bureaucracy, and professional practice are not only explicit rules. They are habits of perception and response.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Habit is the background intelligence through which action usually proceeds before explicit theory appears. (习惯是行动通常在明确理论出现之前得以进行的背景智能。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Instinct (本能; la: instinctus)** suggests natural programming; **Habit (习惯; la: habitus)** is learned, revisable, and socially shaped. (本能暗示自然程序；习惯是习得的、可修正的、由社会塑造的。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** habit displaces the image of the subject as a pure chooser. The subject is a body of trained tendencies. (习惯移置主体作为纯粹选择者的图像。主体是一组被训练出来的倾向。)  
  
### 7. Belief: The Problem of Readiness to Act  
  
`Belief (信念; en: belief)`  
**Definition:** a settled disposition to act, infer, expect, and respond in certain ways. (一种稳定的行动、推论、期待和反应倾向。)  
**Problem solved:** it treats belief not as inert inner representation, but as practical orientation. (它把信念理解为实践取向，而不是惰性的内部表象。)  
**Why needed:** what someone believes is often shown in what they are prepared to do, not merely what they claim. (一个人的信念常由其准备做什么显示，而不只是由其声称什么显示。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing commitment, action, policy, religious life, scientific theory, moral judgment, or institutional practice. (当分析承诺、行动、政策、宗教生活、科学理论、道德判断或制度实践时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
For pragmatism, belief is not only a mental item. It is a rule for action. To believe that a bridge is safe is to be prepared to cross it, recommend it, or rely on it. To believe that equality matters is to be prepared to criticize unequal institutions, not merely praise equality verbally.  
  
This makes belief testable through conduct. A professed belief that never affects action may be rhetorical rather than practical.  
  
**Typical sentence:** A belief is not fully understood until one sees what habits of action it supports. (只有看到一个信念支持什么行动习惯，才能充分理解它。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Opinion (意见; la: opinio)** may be verbally held; **Belief (信念; en: belief)** in pragmatism is a practical disposition. (意见可能只是言语上持有；实用主义中的信念是实践倾向。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** belief becomes embodied in action. Epistemology moves closer to ethics and practice. (信念在行动中具身化。认识论接近伦理学和实践。)  
  
### 8. Doubt: The Problem of Disrupted Habit  
  
`Doubt (怀疑; la: dubitatio; en: doubt)`  
**Definition:** a disturbed state in which settled belief or habit fails and inquiry becomes necessary. (稳定信念或习惯失败并使探究成为必要的受扰状态。)  
**Problem solved:** it distinguishes real doubt from theatrical or merely verbal skepticism. (它把真实怀疑同戏剧化或仅仅口头的怀疑区分开来。)  
**Why needed:** not every imagined skeptical possibility is a genuine problem in practice. (并非每个被想象出的怀疑可能性都是实践中的真实问题。)  
**How to use:** use it when asking whether a doubt actually disrupts inquiry, conduct, or belief. (当追问某种怀疑是否实际打断探究、行为或信念时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Peirce criticizes paper doubt: doubt performed for philosophy but not lived in conduct. A person may say, “maybe the external world does not exist,” but still avoid falling objects, answer messages, eat food, and rely on memory. Pragmatism asks whether the doubt has practical grip.  
  
This does not dismiss skepticism. It disciplines skepticism. A real doubt is one that disturbs practice and requires inquiry.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Doubt becomes philosophically serious when it disrupts settled conduct and demands inquiry. (当怀疑打断稳定行为并要求探究时，它才具有哲学严肃性。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Skepticism (怀疑主义; el: σκέψις)** can be a theoretical position; **Doubt (怀疑; en: doubt)** in pragmatism is a lived disturbance of belief. (怀疑主义可以是一种理论立场；实用主义中的怀疑是信念的被生活的扰动。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** skepticism becomes practical. The question is not merely what can be doubted in abstraction, but what doubt actually does to inquiry. (怀疑主义变得实践化。问题不只是抽象地可以怀疑什么，而是怀疑实际对探究做了什么。)  
  
### 9. Fallibilism: The Problem of Knowledge without Final Certainty  
  
`Fallibilism (可错论; la: fallibilis; en: fallibilism)`  
**Definition:** the view that human beliefs, theories, and inquiries may be rationally warranted while still remaining corrigible and possibly mistaken. (认为人的信念、理论和探究可以具有理性根据，同时仍然可修正且可能错误的观点。)  
**Problem solved:** it avoids both dogmatism and radical skepticism. (它避免独断论和激进怀疑主义。)  
**Why needed:** inquiry needs commitment, but also openness to correction. (探究需要承诺，也需要向修正开放。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing science, law, democracy, moral judgment, interpretation, or historical knowledge under uncertainty. (当分析不确定条件下的科学、法律、民主、道德判断、解释或历史知识时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Fallibilism is one of pragmatism’s central virtues. It says that certainty is not required for rational inquiry. A belief may be the best available conclusion, yet remain revisable. This is how science often works. It also describes legal reasoning, medicine, historical interpretation, and public policy.  
  
This connects fallibilism to abductive reasoning: inquiry often proceeds by selecting the best available explanation under limited evidence, while recognizing that future evidence may overturn it.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Fallibilism allows inquiry to proceed without pretending that its results are final. (可错论允许探究继续进行，而不假装其结果是最终的。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Certainty (确定性; la: certitudo)** seeks impossibility of error; **Fallibilism (可错论; en: fallibilism)** accepts revisability without abandoning rational warrant. (确定性寻求不可能错误；可错论接受可修正性，但不放弃理性根据。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** knowledge becomes provisional without becoming arbitrary. This is one of pragmatism’s strongest answers to both absolutism and relativism. (知识变得暂定，但不变得任意。这是实用主义对绝对主义和相对主义最强的回应之一。)  
  
### 10. Abduction: The Problem of Best Available Explanation  
  
`Abduction (溯因/最佳解释推理; en: abduction)`  
**Definition:** reasoning that moves from surprising or incomplete evidence to the hypothesis that would best explain it. (从令人惊讶或不完整的证据推向最能解释该证据的假说的推理。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains how inquiry can begin when deductive proof and complete induction are unavailable. (它解释在无法获得演绎证明和完整归纳时，探究如何开始。)  
**Why needed:** science, law, diagnosis, history, and everyday reasoning often require hypothesis formation under uncertainty. (科学、法律、诊断、历史和日常推理常需要在不确定条件下形成假说。)  
**How to use:** use it when comparing explanations for a body of evidence. (当比较一组证据的不同解释时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Peirce made abduction central to inquiry. It does not guarantee truth. It generates a plausible hypothesis that can be tested, revised, or replaced. This gives pragmatism a disciplined account of uncertain reasoning.  
  
For example, a doctor does not deduce a diagnosis from symptoms with absolute certainty. A historian does not reconstruct the past by pure observation. A lawyer does not prove every fact by direct access. All use abductive reasoning: what hypothesis best explains the available evidence?  
  
**Typical sentence:** Abduction gives inquiry a way to move intelligently from evidence to hypothesis without claiming final certainty. (溯因使探究能够从证据明智地走向假说，而不声称最终确定性。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Deduction (演绎; la: deductio)** preserves truth from premises to conclusion; **Abduction (溯因; en: abduction)** proposes the best explanation for evidence. (演绎把真从前提保存到结论；溯因提出对证据的最佳解释。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** reasoning becomes experimental. The point is not to escape uncertainty, but to work well within it. (推理变得实验化。重点不是逃离不确定性，而是在不确定性中良好运作。)  
  
### 11. Truth: The Problem of Verification in Practice  
  
`Truth (真理; el: ἀλήθεια; la: veritas; en: truth)`  
**Definition:** in pragmatist terms, not mere usefulness, but what is warranted, verified, or stabilized through successful inquiry and practical testing. (在实用主义中，不是单纯有用性，而是通过成功探究和实践检验而被证成、验证或稳定下来的东西。)  
**Problem solved:** it connects truth to inquiry without reducing truth to subjective preference. (它把真理同探究连接起来，而不把真理化约为主观偏好。)  
**Why needed:** abstract correspondence theories may ignore the concrete processes through which truth is sought, tested, and revised. (抽象符合论可能忽视真理被寻求、检验和修正的具体过程。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing how claims become warranted through investigation, consequences, experiment, and correction. (当分析主张如何通过调查、后果、实验和修正获得证成时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Pragmatist truth is often caricatured. It is not “believe whatever works for you.” A comforting falsehood may be useful in one narrow sense, but it fails under broader inquiry. Pragmatist truth must be tested through experience, consequences, community, evidence, and long-run correction.  
  
For Peirce, truth is connected to the ideal endpoint of inquiry. For James, truth is what proves itself in lived verification. For Dewey, truth is better described as warranted assertibility within inquiry.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Pragmatist truth is not private convenience; it is what survives disciplined inquiry and proves itself in practice. (实用主义真理不是私人便利，而是在有规训的探究中存活并在实践中证明自身的东西。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Correspondence (符合; en: correspondence)** emphasizes relation between proposition and reality; **Pragmatist Truth (实用主义真理; en: pragmatist truth)** emphasizes tested consequences within inquiry. (符合强调命题与现实的关系；实用主义真理强调探究中的被检验后果。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** truth becomes procedural and experimental. It is not detached from life, but also not reducible to immediate success. (真理变得程序化和实验化。它不脱离生活，但也不能化约为直接成功。)  
  
### 12. Experience: The Problem of Worldly Testing  
  
`Experience (经验; la: experientia; en: experience)`  
**Definition:** the lived, practical, experimental, and socially mediated encounter with the world through which beliefs are tested and revised. (信念通过它被检验和修正的、被生活的、实践性的、实验性的且受社会中介的世界遭遇。)  
**Problem solved:** it prevents philosophy from treating thought as detached from worldly contact. (它防止哲学把思想视为脱离世界接触的东西。)  
**Why needed:** inquiry is answerable to what happens when ideas meet resistance, consequences, and use. (探究必须回应观念遭遇阻力、后果和使用时发生的事情。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing learning, testing, experiment, suffering, adjustment, education, democracy, or embodied inquiry. (当分析学习、检验、实验、痛苦、调适、教育、民主或具身探究时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
For pragmatism, experience is not passive reception of sense-data. It is active, experimental, and world-involving. People act, encounter consequences, revise habits, and reorganize situations.  
  
This makes experience different from empiricist data. Experience includes doing, undergoing, testing, feeling, social interaction, and institutional conditions.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Experience is where concepts meet consequences and become answerable to the world. (经验是概念遭遇后果并对世界负责的地方。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Sense-Data (感觉材料; en: sense-data)** suggests discrete mental contents; **Experience (经验; en: experience)** in pragmatism is active transaction with the world. (感觉材料暗示离散的心理内容；实用主义中的经验是同世界的主动交互。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** experience becomes active and experimental, not merely receptive. (经验变得主动且实验化，而非仅仅接受性。)  
  
### 13. Instrumentalism: The Problem of Concepts as Tools  
  
`Instrumentalism (工具主义; en: instrumentalism)`  
**Definition:** the view that concepts, theories, and ideas function as instruments for organizing experience, guiding action, and solving problems. (认为概念、理论和观念作为组织经验、引导行动和解决问题的工具而运作的观点。)  
**Problem solved:** it prevents theories from being treated as sacred mirrors of reality rather than tools of inquiry. (它防止理论被视为现实的神圣镜像，而不是探究工具。)  
**Why needed:** a theory’s worth often lies in what it enables inquiry to do. (理论的价值常在于它使探究能够做什么。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing models, legal concepts, scientific theories, educational categories, or social diagnoses as tools. (当把模型、法律概念、科学理论、教育分类或社会诊断作为工具来分析时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Instrumentalism does not mean theories are merely fictional or arbitrary. A tool can be evaluated. It may be accurate, powerful, misleading, crude, elegant, dangerous, or obsolete. The question is what work it performs.  
  
A medical diagnosis, legal category, economic model, or sociological concept should be judged by its consequences in inquiry and practice. Does it illuminate? Does it predict? Does it distort? Does it govern? Does it harm? Does it open action?  
  
**Typical sentence:** Instrumentalism treats concepts as tools whose value lies in the work they enable and the distortions they avoid. (工具主义把概念视为工具，其价值在于它们使什么工作成为可能，以及避免什么扭曲。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Representation (表征; la: repraesentatio)** suggests mirroring; **Instrument (工具; la: instrumentum)** suggests practical operation. (表征暗示镜像；工具暗示实践操作。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** theory becomes equipment. Philosophy asks not only what a theory says, but what it enables. (理论成为装备。哲学不只追问理论说了什么，也追问它使什么成为可能。)  
  
### 14. Ordinary Language Philosophy: The Problem of Philosophical Misuse  
  
`Ordinary Language Philosophy (日常语言哲学; en: ordinary language philosophy)`  
**Definition:** a philosophical approach that investigates how words actually function in ordinary practices in order to dissolve or clarify philosophical confusions. (一种哲学进路，它考察词语在日常实践中实际如何运作，以消解或澄清哲学混乱。)  
**Problem solved:** it exposes philosophical problems caused by tearing words away from their ordinary use. (它揭示由把词语从日常使用中撕离而产生的哲学问题。)  
**Why needed:** many abstract puzzles arise when language is forced to work outside the practices that give it sense. (许多抽象难题产生于语言被迫在赋予其意义的实践之外运作。)  
**How to use:** use it when a philosophical concept becomes obscure because its everyday grammar has been ignored. (当一个哲学概念因日常语法被忽视而变得晦暗时，应使用这一方法。)  
  
Ordinary language philosophy is associated with the later **Wittgenstein**, **J. L. Austin**, **Gilbert Ryle**, and **P. F. Strawson**. It does not say ordinary language is infallible. It says ordinary language is philosophically instructive because it contains distinctions sedimented in use.  
  
For example, “knowing,” “believing,” “intending,” “promising,” “excusing,” “pretending,” “choosing,” and “being responsible” do not all function like names of inner objects. Their grammar differs. Philosophical confusion often begins when all these words are forced into one model.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Ordinary language philosophy asks how a word functions before turning it into a metaphysical object. (日常语言哲学在把一个词变成形而上学对象之前，先追问它如何运作。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Ideal Language Philosophy (理想语言哲学; en: ideal language philosophy)** seeks formal precision; **Ordinary Language Philosophy (日常语言哲学; en: ordinary language philosophy)** seeks clarification through actual use. (理想语言哲学寻求形式精确性；日常语言哲学通过实际使用寻求澄清。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** philosophy turns from hidden essences to public grammar. Meaning is not primarily inside the mind; it is in use. (哲学从隐藏本质转向公共语法。意义不首先在心灵内部，而在使用中。)  
  
### 15. Use: The Problem of Meaning as Activity  
  
`Use (使用; en: use; de: Gebrauch)`  
**Definition:** the practical role a word, expression, rule, or concept plays in a language-practice. (一个词、表达、规则或概念在语言实践中发挥的实践角色。)  
**Problem solved:** it shifts meaning from inner object or abstract definition to public activity. (它把意义从内部对象或抽象定义转向公共活动。)  
**Why needed:** words mean differently across practices because they are used differently. (词语在不同实践中意义不同，因为它们被不同地使用。)  
**How to use:** use it when asking what a word does in a context: reports, commands, promises, jokes, classifications, excuses, calculations, rituals. (当追问一个词在语境中做什么时，应使用这一概念：报告、命令、承诺、玩笑、分类、辩解、计算、仪式。)  
  
Wittgenstein’s famous lesson is that meaning is often use. A word is not a label attached to a mental object. Its meaning is shown by how it is used in a practice.  
  
The word “game” does not have one strict essence shared by every case. The word “pain” is not learned by inspecting a private inner object. The word “promise” does not merely describe an inner intention; it performs a social act under rules.  
  
**Typical sentence:** To understand a word is to understand how it is used in a practice. (理解一个词，就是理解它如何在实践中被使用。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Reference (指称; de: Bedeutung)** asks what a term points to; **Use (使用; de: Gebrauch)** asks what role the expression plays in practice. (指称追问术语指向什么；使用追问表达在实践中发挥什么角色。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** meaning moves from representation to activity. Language is not only a mirror; it is a set of tools. (意义从表征转向活动。语言不只是镜子，而是一组工具。)  
  
### 16. Language-Game: The Problem of Meaning within Rule-Governed Practice  
  
`Language-Game (语言游戏; de: Sprachspiel; en: language-game)`  
**Definition:** a rule-governed practice in which words, actions, objects, roles, and purposes work together to produce meaning. (一种受规则支配的实践，其中词语、行动、对象、角色和目的共同运作以生产意义。)  
**Problem solved:** it prevents language from being reduced to naming or describing. (它防止语言被化约为命名或描述。)  
**Why needed:** language includes commanding, questioning, calculating, joking, praying, promising, reporting, thanking, ordering, measuring, and storytelling. (语言包括命令、提问、计算、开玩笑、祈祷、承诺、报告、感谢、下令、测量和讲故事。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing a specific practice of speech and action rather than language in general. (当分析具体言说—行动实践，而不是一般语言时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
A language-game is not a trivial game. It names the practical setting in which language has sense. Courtroom language, laboratory language, classroom language, prayer, bargaining, therapy, diagnosis, programming, and joking are different language-games.  
  
A word may move across games and change function. “Guilty” in a courtroom, private conscience, religious confession, and playful teasing is not the same operation.  
  
**Typical sentence:** A language-game is the practice in which words have rules, roles, and consequences. (语言游戏是词语具有规则、角色和后果的实践。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Sentence (句子; en: sentence)** is a linguistic form; **Language-Game (语言游戏; de: Sprachspiel)** is the practice in which that form has a role. (句子是语言形式；语言游戏是该形式拥有角色的实践。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** language becomes plural. There is no single essence of language; there are many practices. (语言变得复数化。语言没有单一本质，而有多种实践。)  
  
### 17. Form of Life: The Problem of Background Agreement  
  
`Form of Life (生活形式; de: Lebensform; en: form of life)`  
**Definition:** the shared human and social background of practices, habits, reactions, institutions, and ways of acting that make language meaningful. (使语言有意义的共享人类与社会背景，包括实践、习惯、反应、制度和行动方式。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains why language depends on lived agreement in practice, not only explicit rules. (它解释语言为何依赖实践中的被生活的同意，而不只依赖明确规则。)  
**Why needed:** rules work only within a background of shared training, reactions, and practices. (规则只有在共享训练、反应和实践背景中才能运作。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing the background world that makes a language-game intelligible. (当分析使一个语言游戏成为可理解的背景世界时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
A form of life is not just lifestyle. It is the background that makes meaning possible. People learn how to count, promise, apologize, measure, accuse, mourn, obey, joke, and doubt through social training. No definition alone can replace this background.  
  
This concept connects Wittgenstein to anthropology, sociology, law, and political theory. A legal rule works only in a form of life where courts, authority, documents, testimony, punishment, and recognition have practical force.  
  
**Typical sentence:** A form of life is the shared background that allows rules and words to have practical sense. (生活形式是使规则和词语具有实践意义的共享背景。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Context (语境; la: contextus)** is the surrounding situation; **Form of Life (生活形式; de: Lebensform)** is the broader practical background that makes language and rules intelligible. (语境是周围情境；生活形式是使语言和规则可理解的更广实践背景。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** meaning becomes social before it becomes theoretical. Philosophy cannot begin from a solitary mind alone. (意义先是社会性的，然后才是理论性的。哲学不能只从孤立心灵开始。)  
  
### 18. Rule-Following: The Problem of Rules without Infinite Interpretation  
  
`Rule-Following (遵循规则; en: rule-following; de: Regelfolgen)`  
**Definition:** the practice of applying rules within shared forms of life, training, correction, and public criteria. (在共享生活形式、训练、纠正和公共标准中应用规则的实践。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains why following a rule cannot consist only in private interpretation. (它解释为什么遵循规则不能只由私人解释构成。)  
**Why needed:** any rule can be interpreted in many ways unless practice fixes what counts as correct continuation. (如果没有实践固定什么算正确继续，任何规则都可以被多种方式解释。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing law, mathematics, language learning, institutions, games, norms, or algorithms. (当分析法律、数学、语言学习、制度、游戏、规范或算法时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Wittgenstein’s rule-following problem is central. A rule does not contain all its future applications in a self-interpreting way. Someone must learn what counts as going on correctly. That learning happens socially.  
  
This matters for law and computation. A statute does not automatically decide every future case. A code specification does not interpret itself outside practices of implementation, testing, and correction. A mathematical series does not teach its continuation without training in the practice of calculation.  
  
**Typical sentence:** A rule is followed not by private interpretation alone, but by public criteria within a practice. (规则不是仅由私人解释来遵循，而是在实践中的公共标准下被遵循。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Rule (规则; la: regula)** is an articulated standard; **Rule-Following (遵循规则; de: Regelfolgen)** is the practice that makes application possible. (规则是被明确表达的标准；遵循规则是使应用成为可能的实践。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** normativity becomes practical. Correctness is not secured by a mental act alone, but by trained participation in a practice. (规范性变得实践化。正确性不由单独心理行为保证，而由受训练的实践参与保证。)  
  
### 19. Family Resemblance: The Problem of Concepts without Essence  
  
`Family Resemblance (家族相似; de: Familienähnlichkeit; en: family resemblance)`  
**Definition:** a pattern in which instances of a concept overlap and resemble one another in multiple ways without sharing one single essence. (一个概念的实例以多种方式重叠和相似，却不共享单一本质的模式。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains concepts that cannot be defined by strict necessary and sufficient conditions. (它解释无法由严格必要充分条件定义的概念。)  
**Why needed:** many ordinary concepts work through overlapping similarities rather than fixed essence. (许多日常概念通过重叠相似性运作，而不是通过固定本质运作。)  
**How to use:** use it when a concept has many cases but no single defining feature common to all. (当一个概念有许多案例却没有所有案例共有的单一规定特征时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Wittgenstein’s example is “game.” Board games, ball games, Olympic games, children’s games, gambling games, and language-games do not all share one essence. They overlap in rules, competition, play, skill, amusement, scoring, and convention, but no one feature appears in every case.  
  
This is important for philosophy because many concepts are over-forced into definitions: art, religion, democracy, intelligence, emotion, disease, law, gender, and personhood may not have one essence.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Family resemblance shows that some concepts work through overlapping similarities rather than strict essence. (家族相似显示某些概念通过重叠相似性而非严格本质运作。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Essence (本质; la: essentia)** seeks a shared defining feature; **Family Resemblance (家族相似; de: Familienähnlichkeit)** identifies overlapping patterns without one essence. (本质寻求共享规定特征；家族相似识别没有单一本质的重叠模式。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** conceptual analysis becomes less essentialist. Philosophy learns to respect flexible ordinary concepts. (概念分析变得较少本质主义。哲学学习尊重灵活的日常概念。)  
  
### 20. Private Language: The Problem of Purely Inner Meaning  
  
`Private Language (私人语言; en: private language; de: Privatsprache)`  
**Definition:** a supposed language whose words refer to wholly private inner experiences accessible only to one individual. (一种假想语言，其词语指向只有一个人能够接近的完全私人内在经验。)  
**Problem solved:** it challenges the idea that meaning can be grounded in purely private mental objects. (它挑战意义能够奠基于纯私人心理对象的观点。)  
**Why needed:** language requires criteria of correct and incorrect use, and purely private criteria collapse. (语言需要正确和错误使用的标准，而纯私人标准会崩塌。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing pain, sensation, consciousness, introspection, or first-person authority. (当分析疼痛、感觉、意识、内省或第一人称权威时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Wittgenstein does not deny inner life. He denies that meaning is fixed by private ostension alone. A person can have pain privately, but the word “pain” is learned in public practices: crying, care, injury, expression, treatment, reassurance, complaint, and response.  
  
This matters for philosophy of mind. Inner experience is real, but language about it is not a private code sealed from all public criteria.  
  
**Typical sentence:** The private language argument does not deny inner experience; it denies that meaning can be secured by purely private criteria. (私人语言论证并不否认内在经验；它否认意义能够由纯私人标准保证。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Privacy of Experience (经验的私人性; en: privacy of experience)** concerns who feels pain; **Private Language (私人语言; en: private language)** concerns whether meaning can be fixed by private criteria alone. (经验的私人性关涉谁感到疼痛；私人语言关涉意义是否能仅由私人标准固定。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** subjectivity becomes public in its grammar. Even first-person language belongs to shared forms of life. (主体性在其语法上变得公共。即使第一人称语言也属于共享生活形式。)  
  
### 21. Speech Act: The Problem of Doing Things with Words  
  
`Speech Act (言语行为; en: speech act)`  
**Definition:** an act performed through speaking, such as promising, ordering, warning, apologizing, naming, sentencing, marrying, or declaring. (通过说话而执行的行动，如承诺、命令、警告、道歉、命名、判决、结婚或宣布。)  
**Problem solved:** it shows that language does not only describe reality; it can also act within reality. (它显示语言不只描述现实，也能在现实中行动。)  
**Why needed:** many utterances create obligations, permissions, statuses, relations, or institutional effects. (许多话语会创造义务、许可、地位、关系或制度效果。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing law, ritual, contract, promise, apology, threat, command, consent, or institutional declaration. (当分析法律、仪式、契约、承诺、道歉、威胁、命令、同意或制度宣布时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
J. L. Austin’s central lesson is that saying can be doing. “I promise” does not merely report an inner state. Under the right conditions, it creates a commitment. “I now pronounce you married” changes legal and social status if uttered by the right person in the right institution. “Guilty” can transform a defendant’s legal situation.  
  
This concept links ordinary language to law, gender theory, ritual, and politics.  
  
**Typical sentence:** A speech act is an utterance that performs an action under recognizable conditions. (言语行为是在可识别条件下执行行动的话语。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Constative (陈述性话语; en: constative)** says what is the case; **Performative (施为性话语; en: performative)** does something by being said. (陈述性话语说明事实如何；施为性话语通过被说出而做事。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** language becomes performative. Words do not only represent social reality; they help make it. (语言变得施为化。词语不只表征社会现实，也帮助制造社会现实。)  
  
### 22. Performative: The Problem of Conditions for Successful Saying  
  
`Performative (施为性话语; en: performative)`  
**Definition:** an utterance that performs the act it names or enacts, under appropriate conventional conditions. (一种在适当约定条件下执行其所命名或实施之行动的话语。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains why some utterances succeed or fail not by truth-value, but by felicity conditions. (它解释为什么某些话语不是按真值，而是按适切条件成功或失败。)  
**Why needed:** promises, contracts, declarations, apologies, oaths, verdicts, and consent depend on social rules and uptake. (承诺、契约、宣布、道歉、誓言、裁决和同意依赖社会规则和接受。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing whether speech has the authority, context, procedure, and uptake needed to perform an act. (当分析话语是否具有执行行动所需的权威、语境、程序和接受时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
A performative can fail. Austin calls this infelicity. A person without authority cannot successfully declare a court in session. A forced “I consent” may not count as valid consent. An apology may fail if conditions of responsibility, recognition, and repair are absent.  
  
This makes performativity highly useful for feminist, queer, legal, and political theory. Gender performativity, legal status, citizenship, marriage, naming, and testimony all involve repeated social acts under rules.  
  
**Typical sentence:** A performative succeeds not by describing a fact, but by satisfying the conditions under which saying counts as doing. (施为性话语不是通过描述事实而成功，而是通过满足“说即做”的条件而成功。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Truth-Condition (真值条件; en: truth-condition)** asks when a statement is true; **Felicity Condition (适切条件; en: felicity condition)** asks when a performative act succeeds. (真值条件追问陈述何时为真；适切条件追问施为行为何时成功。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** performativity connects ordinary language philosophy with social ontology. Institutions are partly built by successful speech acts. (施为性把日常语言哲学同社会本体论连接起来。制度部分由成功的言语行为构成。)  
  
### 23. Category Mistake: The Problem of Misplacing Concepts  
  
`Category Mistake (范畴错误; en: category mistake)`  
**Definition:** an error that occurs when a concept is applied as if it belonged to a different logical or practical category than it actually does. (当一个概念被当作属于不同于其实际所属的逻辑或实践范畴而被应用时发生的错误。)  
**Problem solved:** it diagnoses philosophical confusion caused by treating one kind of thing as another kind. (它诊断把一种东西当作另一种东西处理所造成的哲学混乱。)  
**Why needed:** many metaphysical puzzles arise from forcing concepts into the wrong grammar. (许多形而上学难题来自把概念强行放入错误语法。)  
**How to use:** use it when a question assumes that something must be an object, place, substance, event, or inner item when it is not. (当一个问题预设某物必须是对象、地点、实体、事件或内部物，而它并非如此时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Gilbert Ryle’s classic example is a visitor shown the colleges, libraries, laboratories, and offices of a university, then asking, “But where is the university?” The mistake is treating the university as another object alongside its institutions, rather than the organized whole.  
  
Ryle applies this to mind. The mind is not a ghostly object inside the body. Many mental terms describe abilities, dispositions, practices, and patterns of conduct.  
  
**Typical sentence:** A category mistake occurs when philosophy looks for an object where the grammar calls for a practice, capacity, role, or institution. (当哲学在语法要求实践、能力、角色或制度之处寻找对象时，范畴错误就发生了。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Factual Error (事实错误; en: factual error)** gets a fact wrong; **Category Mistake (范畴错误; en: category mistake)** uses the wrong kind of concept. (事实错误弄错事实；范畴错误使用了错误种类的概念。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** philosophy becomes grammatical therapy. Some problems are not solved by discovering hidden objects, but by correcting conceptual placement. (哲学成为语法治疗。某些问题不是通过发现隐藏对象解决，而是通过修正概念位置解决。)  
  
### 24. Therapy: The Problem of Dissolving Pseudo-Problems  
  
`Therapy (治疗; el: θεραπεία; en: therapy; de: Therapie)`  
**Definition:** Wittgenstein’s image of philosophy as the treatment of conceptual confusion by returning words to their actual use. (维特根斯坦把哲学理解为通过让词语回到其实际使用来处理概念混乱的图像。)  
**Problem solved:** it dissolves problems created by language going on holiday. (它消解语言“放假”时制造的问题。)  
**Why needed:** philosophy often becomes trapped by pictures: mind as inner theater, meaning as object, rule as rail, essence as hidden core. (哲学常被图像困住：心灵作为内部剧场、意义作为对象、规则作为轨道、本质作为隐藏核心。)  
**How to use:** use it when a philosophical problem may result from misleading grammar rather than deep metaphysical reality. (当一个哲学问题可能来自误导性语法，而非深层形而上学现实时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Therapy does not mean philosophy becomes shallow. It means philosophy must examine its own compulsions. Why does a word tempt thought in a certain direction? Why does “meaning” seem like an object? Why does “mind” seem like a place? Why does “rule” seem to contain all applications? Why does “self” seem like an inner owner?  
  
The therapeutic task is to loosen the grip of these pictures.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Philosophical therapy does not answer every question directly; it shows when the question was produced by a misleading picture. (哲学治疗并不直接回答每个问题；它显示何时问题是由误导性图像生产出来的。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Theory-Building (理论建构; en: theory-building)** constructs explanations; **Therapy (治疗; de: Therapie)** removes conceptual compulsions that make false theories seem necessary. (理论建构构造解释；治疗移除使错误理论显得必要的概念强迫。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** philosophy becomes self-critical about its own language. The philosopher is not always a builder; sometimes the philosopher is a physician of concepts. (哲学对自身语言变得自我批判。哲学家不总是建造者；有时是概念医生。)  
  
### 25. The Pragmatist and Ordinary-Language Diagnostic Method  
  
Pragmatist and ordinary-language analysis should not become anti-theory. The method is more exact.  
  
A strong pragmatist reading asks:  
  
**What practical difference does this concept make?**  
(这个概念造成什么实践差异？)  
  
**What habits of action does this belief support?**  
(这个信念支持什么行动习惯？)  
  
**What problem does this theory help solve?**  
(这个理论帮助解决什么问题？)  
  
**What consequences follow if this claim is accepted?**  
(如果接受这个主张，会产生什么后果？)  
  
**How could inquiry test, revise, or abandon it?**  
(探究如何检验、修正或放弃它？)  
  
A strong ordinary-language reading asks:  
  
**How is this word actually used?**  
(这个词实际上如何被使用？)  
  
**What language-game gives it sense?**  
(什么语言游戏赋予它意义？)  
  
**What form of life supports that language-game?**  
(什么生活形式支撑这个语言游戏？)  
  
**Is the problem caused by a category mistake or misleading grammar?**  
(这个问题是否由范畴错误或误导性语法造成？)  
  
**Does this word describe, command, promise, authorize, excuse, judge, or perform?**  
(这个词是在描述、命令、承诺、授权、辩解、判断，还是施为？)  
  
**Typical sentence:** Pragmatist and ordinary-language reading asks what a concept does, where it is used, and what confusion appears when it is pulled out of practice. (实用主义与日常语言阅读追问一个概念做什么、在哪里被使用，以及当它被抽离实践时出现什么混乱。)  
  
### 26. The Tool-Map of Pragmatism and Ordinary Language Philosophy  
  
Use pragmatist and ordinary-language vocabulary diagnostically. The core question is usually not “what is the hidden essence?” but “how does this concept work in practice?”  
  
**If the text asks what practical difference a concept makes**, look for **Pragmatism (实用主义; en: pragmatism)**, **Consequence (后果; en: consequence)**, and **Practice (实践; en: practice)**.  
(如果文本追问一个概念造成什么实践差异，应寻找实用主义、后果和实践问题。)  
  
**If the text treats thinking as problem-solving**, look for **Inquiry (探究; en: inquiry)**, **Experience (经验; en: experience)**, and **Instrumentalism (工具主义; en: instrumentalism)**.  
(如果文本把思考视为问题解决，应寻找探究、经验和工具主义问题。)  
  
**If the text analyzes action-dispositions**, look for **Habit (习惯; en: habit)** and **Belief (信念; en: belief)**.  
(如果文本分析行动倾向，应寻找习惯和信念问题。)  
  
**If the text accepts revisability without skepticism**, look for **Fallibilism (可错论; en: fallibilism)**.  
(如果文本在接受可修正性的同时不滑入怀疑主义，应寻找可错论问题。)  
  
**If the text compares explanations under uncertainty**, look for **Abduction (溯因; en: abduction)**.  
(如果文本在不确定条件下比较解释，应寻找溯因问题。)  
  
**If the text clarifies meaning through actual use**, look for **Ordinary Language Philosophy (日常语言哲学; en: ordinary language philosophy)** and **Use (使用; de: Gebrauch)**.  
(如果文本通过实际使用澄清意义，应寻找日常语言哲学和使用问题。)  
  
**If the text analyzes rule-governed speech practices**, look for **Language-Game (语言游戏; de: Sprachspiel)** and **Form of Life (生活形式; de: Lebensform)**.  
(如果文本分析受规则支配的言说实践，应寻找语言游戏和生活形式问题。)  
  
**If the text asks how rules apply**, look for **Rule-Following (遵循规则; de: Regelfolgen)**.  
(如果文本追问规则如何应用，应寻找遵循规则问题。)  
  
**If the text resists essential definitions**, look for **Family Resemblance (家族相似; de: Familienähnlichkeit)**.  
(如果文本抵抗本质主义定义，应寻找家族相似问题。)  
  
**If the text challenges purely private meaning**, look for **Private Language (私人语言; de: Privatsprache)**.  
(如果文本挑战纯私人意义，应寻找私人语言问题。)  
  
**If the text analyzes words as actions**, look for **Speech Act (言语行为; en: speech act)** and **Performative (施为性话语; en: performative)**.  
(如果文本把词语分析为行动，应寻找言语行为和施为性话语问题。)  
  
**If the text diagnoses misplaced concepts**, look for **Category Mistake (范畴错误; en: category mistake)** and **Therapy (治疗; de: Therapie)**.  
(如果文本诊断概念错置，应寻找范畴错误和治疗问题。)  
  
### 27. The Genealogical Point of Part 18  
  
Pragmatism and ordinary language philosophy transform the philosophical language of meaning. Greek philosophy sought **logos**, definition, essence, and rational account. Latin metaphysics stabilized substance, essence, and law. Early modern philosophy searched for certainty in the subject and method. Kant asked for conditions of possible experience. German Idealism made reason historical. Marx, Nietzsche, Freud, Foucault, Derrida, feminism, and postcolonial theory exposed hidden structures of power, desire, difference, gender, empire, and exclusion.  
  
Pragmatism and ordinary language philosophy add:  
  
**Concepts must be tested by their use, consequences, practices, and forms of life.**  
(概念必须由其使用、后果、实践和生活形式来检验。)  
  
The guiding thesis is:  
  
**Pragmatist and ordinary-language philosophy turns philosophical vocabulary into a problem of use: to understand a concept is to ask what practical difference it makes, what inquiry it guides, what habits it forms, what language-game gives it sense, what form of life supports it, and what confusion appears when it is abstracted from practice.**  
(实用主义与日常语言哲学把哲学词汇转化为使用问题：理解一个概念，就是追问它造成什么实践差异，引导什么探究，形成什么习惯，什么语言游戏赋予它意义，什么生活形式支撑它，以及当它被抽离实践时出现什么混乱。)  
  
This grammar prepares the next stage: **Contemporary Critical Vocabulary: Technology, Data, Platform, Anthropocene**. Once pragmatism and ordinary language philosophy return meaning to practice, the next chapter can ask how contemporary practices are reorganized by platforms, data, algorithms, ecological crisis, and technological infrastructures.  
  
The pragmatist-ordinary-language question remains one of the strongest tools for philosophical reading:  
  
**What does this concept do in practice, what form of life makes it intelligible, and what philosophical confusion appears when it is treated as an abstract essence rather than a tool of use?**  
(这个概念在实践中做什么？什么生活形式使它成为可理解的？当它被当作抽象本质而非使用工具时，会出现什么哲学混乱？)  
  
## Part 19. Contemporary Critical Vocabulary: Technology, Data, Platform, Anthropocene  
  
This chapter explains contemporary critical vocabulary for a world increasingly organized by **technology**, **data**, **platforms**, **algorithms**, **automation**, **surveillance**, **infrastructure**, **artificial intelligence**, and **ecological crisis**. **Heidegger** for technology as enframing, **Critical Theory** for instrumental reason, **Foucault** for power/knowledge and governmentality, **Derrida** for archive, trace, iterability, and signature, **feminism** for bodies and hidden labor, **postcolonial theory** for extractive global hierarchy, and **pragmatism** for use, consequences, and practice.  
  
The central question is:  
  
**What form of life is produced when human action, attention, desire, labor, identity, risk, and environment are reorganized by computational systems?**  
(当人的行动、注意力、欲望、劳动、身份、风险和环境被计算系统重组时，会生产出什么生活形式？)  
  
The central vocabulary is **Technology**, **Technics**, **Enframing**, **Infrastructure**, **Data**, **Datafication**, **Database**, **Metadata**, **Archive**, **Algorithm**, **Algorithmic Governance**, **Model**, **Prediction**, **Classification**, **Automation**, **Human Oversight**, **Opacity**, **Explainability**, **Accountability**, **Platform**, **Platform Capitalism**, **Surveillance Capitalism**, **Attention Economy**, **Digital Labor**, **AI Agent**, **Alignment**, **Posthuman**, **Cyborg**, **Anthropocene**, **Capitalocene**, **Extraction**, and **Planetary Crisis**.  
  
Surveillance, algorithmic fairness, environmental cost, automation’s labor implications, and AI governance require philosophy, sociology, political economy, and law rather than only technical CS treatment.  They also emphasize that computation works on **representations** rather than the world directly, and that representation is not neutral because it determines what can be expressed, made efficient, ignored, or made error-prone.  
  
The operational function of this chapter is exact: use contemporary critical vocabulary when the problem is **how technical systems organize power, knowledge, labor, attention, bodies, environments, and future possibilities**. (当问题是技术系统如何组织权力、知识、劳动、注意力、身体、环境和未来可能性时，应使用当代批判词汇。)  
  
### 1. The Problem-Situation: Technical Systems Are Social Forms  
  
A weak analysis says: technology is a tool. A stronger analysis says: technology is a tool embedded in institutions. A still stronger analysis says: technology reorganizes what counts as action, knowledge, relation, identity, labor, risk, and world.  
  
The contemporary problem is not only that people use devices. The problem is that social reality is increasingly formatted by computational systems: databases classify persons; platforms allocate visibility; algorithms rank attention; models predict behavior; metrics govern work; sensors collect traces; infrastructures condition movement; AI systems generate language, images, code, and decisions; climate systems register the cumulative effect of industrial life.  
  
The central contemporary question is therefore:  
  
**What becomes thinkable, measurable, governable, profitable, and disposable once the world is represented as data?**  
(一旦世界被表征为数据，什么会变得可思考、可测量、可治理、可盈利和可抛弃？)  
  
This question joins Heidegger, Marx, Foucault, Derrida, feminism, postcolonial theory, and pragmatism. Heidegger asks how technology reveals beings. Marx asks how capital extracts value. Foucault asks how knowledge makes populations governable. Derrida asks what archive and trace preserve or exclude. Feminism asks whose labor and body are hidden. Postcolonial theory asks what extraction and global hierarchy support the system. Pragmatism asks what the system does in practice.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Contemporary critical theory treats technical systems not as neutral tools, but as infrastructures that reorganize action, knowledge, labor, and subjectivity. (当代批判理论不把技术系统视为中立工具，而把它们视为重组行动、知识、劳动和主体性的基础设施。)  
  
### 2. Technology: The Problem of Organized Means  
  
`Technology (技术; el: τέχνη; de: Technik)`  
**Definition:** organized means, techniques, devices, systems, and knowledges through which human beings transform and regulate the world. (人通过它们转化并规制世界的有组织手段、技艺、装置、系统和知识。)  
**Problem solved:** it names the material and procedural mediation between intention and world. (它命名意图与世界之间的物质和程序性中介。)  
**Why needed:** modern power often acts through systems, devices, standards, protocols, interfaces, and infrastructures rather than direct command alone. (现代权力常通过系统、装置、标准、协议、界面和基础设施运作，而不只是通过直接命令。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing tools, machines, systems, protocols, infrastructures, AI, platforms, medicine, weapons, media, or environmental control. (当分析工具、机器、系统、协议、基础设施、AI、平台、医学、武器、媒体或环境控制时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Technology is not only applied science. It is also social organization. A smartphone is not merely hardware. It is supply chain, software ecosystem, operating system, app economy, interface discipline, communication norm, surveillance surface, labor network, and attention machine.  
  
Technology therefore must be read at several levels: material device, technical system, institutional arrangement, social practice, economic model, and mode of subject formation.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Technology is not simply an instrument used by society; it is one of the ways society organizes itself. (技术不只是社会所使用的工具；它也是社会组织自身的方式之一。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Tool (工具; en: tool)** suggests an object controlled by a user; **Technology (技术; de: Technik)** names a broader system of means, practices, institutions, and world-relation. (工具暗示由使用者控制的对象；技术命名更广的手段、实践、制度和世界关系系统。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** technology moves from craft to system. Modern technology is no longer only local tool-use; it becomes infrastructure, administration, automation, and planetary transformation. (技术从技艺转向系统。现代技术不再只是局部工具使用，而成为基础设施、行政管理、自动化和行星尺度转化。)  
  
### 3. Technics: The Problem of Human-Technical Co-Formation  
  
`Technics (技艺/技术性; el: τέχνη; fr: technique)`  
**Definition:** the broader condition of technical mediation through which human capacities, memory, action, and social life are formed. (一种更广泛的技术中介条件，人类能力、记忆、行动和社会生活通过它被形成。)  
**Problem solved:** it prevents technology from being treated as external to human life. (它防止技术被视为外在于人类生活。)  
**Why needed:** writing, tools, calendars, maps, clocks, machines, databases, and AI systems do not merely serve humans; they shape what humans can remember, coordinate, imagine, and do. (书写、工具、历法、地图、时钟、机器、数据库和 AI 系统不只是服务人类；它们塑造人类能够记忆、协调、想象和行动的方式。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing technical mediation as constitutive of subjectivity, society, and memory. (当分析技术中介如何构成主体性、社会和记忆时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Technics is useful because it avoids a false opposition between natural humanity and artificial tools. Human beings are tool-making, symbol-using, memory-externalizing beings. Writing changes memory. Clocks change time-discipline. Maps change territory. Databases change administration. Platforms change sociality. AI changes language-production and cognitive delegation.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Technics names the technical mediation through which human capacities are extended, formatted, and constrained. (技术性命名人类能力借以被扩展、格式化和限制的技术中介。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Technology (技术; de: Technik)** often names concrete systems or devices; **Technics (技艺/技术性; fr: technique)** names the broader technical condition of human life. (技术常命名具体系统或装置；技术性命名人类生活的更广技术条件。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** the human becomes technically mediated. The question is no longer human versus machine, but what forms of human-machine co-formation are being built. (人变得由技术中介。问题不再是人与机器的对立，而是正在建构什么人机共同形成形式。)  
  
### 4. Enframing: The Problem of World as Resource  
  
`Enframing (集置; de: Gestell)`  
**Definition:** Heidegger’s term for the modern technological mode of revealing in which beings appear primarily as resources to be ordered, stored, optimized, and used. (海德格尔用来指现代技术性开显方式的术语，其中存在者主要显现为可被订置、储备、优化和使用的资源。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains technology not merely as devices, but as a way the world becomes intelligible. (它把技术解释为一种世界变得可理解的方式，而不只是装置集合。)  
**Why needed:** modern systems often reveal forests as timber, rivers as energy, persons as users, attention as inventory, behavior as data, and life as optimization target. (现代系统常把森林显现为木材、河流显现为能源、人显现为用户、注意力显现为库存、行为显现为数据、生命显现为优化目标。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing technological rationality as a mode of revealing and ordering reality. (当把技术理性分析为开显和订置现实的方式时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Enframing does not mean technology is evil. It means technology reveals the world under a specific grammar: availability, calculability, control, efficiency, reserve. This grammar is powerful. It builds hospitals, networks, logistics, energy systems, and AI. It also risks reducing beings to standing-reserve.  
  
In contemporary digital systems, enframing appears as data capture, metricization, optimization, personalization, prediction, and automated intervention.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Enframing makes the world appear as a field of resources available for ordering and optimization. (集置使世界显现为可供订置和优化的资源场。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Instrumental Reason (工具理性; de: instrumentelle Vernunft)** calculates means to ends; **Enframing (集置; de: Gestell)** names the deeper disclosure in which beings appear as orderable resources. (工具理性计算达到目的的手段；集置命名存在者显现为可订置资源的更深开显方式。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** Heidegger’s technology critique prepares later critiques of datafication and platform governance. The world is not only used; it is formatted to be usable. (海德格尔的技术批判为后来的数据化和平台治理批判做准备。世界不只是被使用；它被格式化为可使用。)  
  
### 5. Infrastructure: The Problem of Invisible Conditions  
  
`Infrastructure (基础设施; la: infra + structura; en: infrastructure)`  
**Definition:** the material, technical, institutional, and logistical systems that make social action possible while often remaining backgrounded. (使社会行动成为可能却常停留在背景中的物质、技术、制度和物流系统。)  
**Problem solved:** it reveals the hidden conditions behind ordinary functioning. (它揭示日常运作背后的隐藏条件。)  
**Why needed:** roads, grids, cloud systems, protocols, databases, logistics, payment systems, identity systems, and standards shape what can happen. (道路、电网、云系统、协议、数据库、物流、支付系统、身份系统和标准塑造什么能够发生。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing background systems that condition action, access, dependency, resilience, and failure. (当分析制约行动、可及性、依赖、韧性和失败的背景系统时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Infrastructure becomes visible when it breaks. A payment outage, cloud failure, blocked port, collapsed bridge, power failure, DNS problem, or model-serving failure reveals how much action was dependent on hidden systems.  
  
Infrastructure is political because it distributes access. It decides who can move, connect, pay, speak, authenticate, store, compute, and be recognized.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Infrastructure is power in background form: it governs by making some actions easy, some difficult, and some impossible. (基础设施是背景形式的权力：它通过使某些行动容易、某些行动困难、某些行动不可能来治理。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Object (对象; la: obiectum)** is foregrounded; **Infrastructure (基础设施; en: infrastructure)** is the background condition that makes foreground objects and actions work. (对象处于前景；基础设施是使前景对象和行动得以运作的背景条件。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** power moves from sovereign command to logistical condition. To control infrastructure is to control possibility. (权力从主权命令转向物流性条件。控制基础设施就是控制可能性。)  
  
### 6. Data: The Problem of Given That Is Made  
  
`Data (数据; la: datum, “that which is given”)`  
**Definition:** recorded, structured, or processable representations treated as input for storage, analysis, inference, prediction, or decision. (被记录、结构化或可处理的表征，被作为存储、分析、推理、预测或决策的输入。)  
**Problem solved:** it names the basic material of computational knowledge. (它命名计算性知识的基本材料。)  
**Why needed:** contemporary institutions increasingly govern through records, traces, metrics, profiles, scores, and datasets. (当代制度越来越通过记录、痕迹、指标、画像、评分和数据集进行治理。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing records, datasets, digital traces, sensors, profiles, statistics, machine learning, or administrative classification. (当分析记录、数据集、数字痕迹、传感器、画像、统计、机器学习或行政分类时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
The Latin **datum** means “given,” but data is rarely simply given. It is produced. Someone chooses what to collect, how to encode, what to exclude, what categories to impose, what errors to tolerate, what proxies to accept, and what purposes the data will serve.  
  
Computation works on representations of the world, and representation is not neutral because it determines what can be expressed, made efficient, ignored, or made error-prone.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Data is not raw reality; it is reality captured under a scheme of representation. (数据不是原始现实；它是在某种表征方案下被捕获的现实。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Fact (事实; la: factum)** is something taken to be the case; **Data (数据; la: datum)** is a recorded representation formatted for processing. (事实是被认为成立之事；数据是被格式化为可处理对象的记录表征。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** knowledge becomes computational. The archive no longer only stores documents; it becomes processable, searchable, inferential, and predictive. (知识变得计算化。档案不再只存储文献；它变得可处理、可搜索、可推理和可预测。)  
  
### 7. Datafication: The Problem of Turning Life into Data  
  
`Datafication (数据化; en: datafication)`  
**Definition:** the process by which actions, bodies, relations, environments, preferences, movements, and affects are converted into data. (行动、身体、关系、环境、偏好、移动和情感被转化为数据的过程。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains how previously informal or embodied life becomes measurable, comparable, and governable. (它解释此前非正式或具身的生活如何变得可测量、可比较和可治理。)  
**Why needed:** platforms, states, firms, schools, hospitals, and workplaces increasingly depend on data extraction and analysis. (平台、国家、企业、学校、医院和工作场所越来越依赖数据提取与分析。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing quantified self, social media traces, workplace metrics, learning analytics, health tracking, smart cities, or behavioral profiling. (当分析量化自我、社交媒体痕迹、工作场所指标、学习分析、健康追踪、智慧城市或行为画像时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Datafication is not mere measurement. It changes what is measured. Once behavior becomes data, it can be stored, ranked, sold, predicted, optimized, policed, and fed back into the behavior itself.  
  
For example, reading becomes engagement data. Movement becomes location data. Friendship becomes social graph. Work becomes productivity metric. Health becomes risk profile. Attention becomes ad inventory. Desire becomes recommendation signal.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Datafication turns lived activity into processable traces that can be stored, compared, predicted, and acted upon. (数据化把被生活的活动转化为可处理痕迹，使其能够被存储、比较、预测和干预。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Measurement (测量; en: measurement)** quantifies selected properties; **Datafication (数据化; en: datafication)** reorganizes practices so that they continuously produce exploitable data. (测量量化被选择的属性；数据化重组实践，使其持续生产可利用数据。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** Foucault’s examination becomes digital and continuous. The file becomes the profile; the profile becomes actionable. (福柯的考试/检查变得数字化且连续。档案变成画像；画像变成可行动对象。)  
  
### 8. Database: The Problem of Organized Memory  
  
`Database (数据库; en: database)`  
**Definition:** an organized system for storing, structuring, querying, updating, and relating data. (用于存储、结构化、查询、更新和关联数据的有组织系统。)  
**Problem solved:** it makes large-scale memory operational. (它使大规模记忆变得可操作。)  
**Why needed:** modern institutions require persistent, queryable, relational, and governable records. (现代制度需要持久、可查询、可关联和可治理的记录。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing institutional memory, records, identity systems, surveillance, administration, platforms, or AI training data. (当分析制度记忆、记录、身份系统、监视、行政、平台或 AI 训练数据时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
A database is not neutral storage. Its schema determines what kinds of entities exist, what relations matter, what histories can be retrieved, what errors persist, and what actions can be automated. In this sense, a database is both technical and ontological. It defines a world of objects and relations.  
  
A person in a database may become user, patient, suspect, applicant, customer, debtor, citizen, migrant, worker, risk, or target. Each database role has consequences.  
  
**Typical sentence:** A database is an operational ontology: it defines what entities exist for a system and how they can be acted upon. (数据库是一种操作性本体论：它定义系统中的实体是什么，以及这些实体如何可被行动作用。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Archive (档案; fr: archive)** governs preservation and authority of records; **Database (数据库; en: database)** makes records structured, queryable, updateable, and operational. (档案规制记录的保存和权威；数据库使记录结构化、可查询、可更新并可操作。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** institutional memory becomes executable. Records no longer merely testify; they trigger actions. (制度记忆变得可执行。记录不再只是作证；它们触发行动。)  
  
### 9. Metadata: The Problem of Data about Relations  
  
`Metadata (元数据; en: metadata)`  
**Definition:** data about data: information concerning origin, time, location, format, relation, author, access, device, or context. (关于数据的数据：涉及来源、时间、地点、格式、关系、作者、访问、设备或语境的信息。)  
**Problem solved:** it reveals that context itself can be captured and analyzed. (它揭示语境本身也可以被捕获和分析。)  
**Why needed:** metadata often exposes patterns, relations, and behavior even when content is unavailable. (即使内容不可得，元数据也常暴露模式、关系和行为。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing surveillance, communication records, platform analytics, digital archives, provenance, or evidentiary chains. (当分析监视、通信记录、平台分析、数字档案、来源或证据链时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Metadata is powerful because it converts context into information. Who contacted whom, when, from where, how often, through what device, in what sequence, and with what response can matter as much as message content.  
  
For Derrida, context is never finally closed. In digital systems, context becomes a new object of capture. This creates a strange reversal: systems try to stabilize context by recording more traces, yet each trace generates further metadata.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Metadata turns context into data and therefore makes relation itself governable. (元数据把语境转化为数据，因此使关系本身变得可治理。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Content (内容; en: content)** is the message or object; **Metadata (元数据; en: metadata)** records the conditions, relations, and traces around it. (内容是信息或对象本身；元数据记录其周围的条件、关系和痕迹。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** surveillance no longer requires reading everything. Patterns of relation can become enough. (监视不再需要阅读一切。关系模式本身就可能足够。)  
  
### 10. Algorithm: The Problem of Formal Procedure  
  
`Algorithm (算法; ar: نسبة إلى الخوارزمي, al-Khwārizmī; en: algorithm)`  
**Definition:** a finite procedure or rule-governed sequence for transforming inputs into outputs. (一种有限程序或受规则支配的序列，用于把输入转化为输出。)  
**Problem solved:** it names procedural action that can be specified, repeated, automated, and scaled. (它命名可被规定、重复、自动化和扩展的程序性行动。)  
**Why needed:** computational systems act through procedures that classify, rank, optimize, recommend, filter, detect, generate, and decide. (计算系统通过程序进行分类、排序、优化、推荐、过滤、检测、生成和决策。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing computational procedure, ranking systems, recommendation, automation, search, classification, or decision support. (当分析计算程序、排序系统、推荐、自动化、搜索、分类或决策支持时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
An algorithm is not automatically political. But algorithms become political when embedded in institutions that distribute visibility, credit, policing, insurance, employment, admission, welfare, speech, or access.  
  
The critical question is not simply “what is the code?” It is: what inputs are used, what objective is optimized, what proxies stand in for values, what errors are tolerated, who is affected, who can contest, and what institution acts on the output?  
  
**Typical sentence:** An algorithm becomes a social power when its outputs are connected to institutional action. (当算法输出同制度行动连接时，算法就成为社会权力。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Procedure (程序; en: procedure)** is a general sequence of steps; **Algorithm (算法; en: algorithm)** is a formalizable computational procedure with specified input-output behavior. (程序是一般步骤序列；算法是具有指定输入—输出行为的可形式化计算程序。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** rules become executable at scale. Bureaucratic classification becomes computational classification. (规则变得可大规模执行。官僚分类变成计算分类。)  
  
### 11. Algorithmic Governance: The Problem of Automated Rule  
  
`Algorithmic Governance (算法治理; en: algorithmic governance)`  
**Definition:** the organization of conduct, access, visibility, risk, and decision-making through computational systems. (通过计算系统组织行为、可及性、可见性、风险和决策。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains governance that operates through ranking, scoring, filtering, recommending, predicting, and automated intervention. (它解释通过排序、评分、过滤、推荐、预测和自动干预而运作的治理。)  
**Why needed:** institutions increasingly govern through data-driven systems rather than explicit human judgment alone. (制度越来越通过数据驱动系统进行治理，而不只是通过明确的人类判断。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing welfare algorithms, policing systems, credit scoring, content moderation, hiring tools, educational analytics, immigration risk, or platform ranking. (当分析福利算法、警务系统、信用评分、内容审核、招聘工具、教育分析、移民风险或平台排序时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Algorithmic governance is Foucauldian and pragmatist at once. It produces knowledge about subjects and changes what happens to them. It also must be evaluated by consequences: who is helped, who is harmed, who is misclassified, who can appeal, who is made invisible.  
  
It often appears efficient, objective, and scalable. But efficiency may hide political choice. Objectivity may hide biased representation. Scale may multiply harm.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Algorithmic governance governs by converting persons and actions into data, then acting on the classifications produced from that data. (算法治理通过把人和行动转化为数据，再根据由数据产生的分类采取行动。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Bureaucratic Governance (官僚治理; en: bureaucratic governance)** acts through files, rules, offices, and officials; **Algorithmic Governance (算法治理; en: algorithmic governance)** acts through data pipelines, models, scores, rankings, and automated or semi-automated decisions. (官僚治理通过档案、规则、办公室和官员行动；算法治理通过数据管道、模型、评分、排序和自动或半自动决策行动。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** Foucault’s governmentality becomes computational. Subjects are governed through environments of prediction and feedback. (福柯的治理术变得计算化。主体通过预测与反馈环境被治理。)  
  
### 12. Model: The Problem of Simplified World  
  
`Model (模型; la: modulus; en: model)`  
**Definition:** a simplified representation of a system, relation, process, or pattern used for explanation, prediction, simulation, or decision. (用于解释、预测、模拟或决策的关于系统、关系、过程或模式的简化表征。)  
**Problem solved:** it allows inquiry and action under complexity by selecting what matters. (它通过选择重要内容，使复杂性条件下的探究和行动成为可能。)  
**Why needed:** no model contains the whole world; it preserves some properties and discards others. (没有模型包含整个世界；模型保留某些属性并舍弃另一些属性。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing scientific models, machine learning models, economic models, climate models, risk models, or social simulations. (当分析科学模型、机器学习模型、经济模型、气候模型、风险模型或社会模拟时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
A model is always a reduction. **Reduction** is a deep first principle: one problem is transformed into another, but the mature question is always what the transformation preserves and what it discards.  This is also the critical theory of models.  
  
A model may be useful and dangerous at the same time. It can reveal pattern, guide intervention, and coordinate action. It can also erase context, misrepresent minority cases, naturalize assumptions, and produce self-fulfilling classifications.  
  
**Typical sentence:** A model is powerful because it simplifies; it is dangerous for the same reason. (模型因为简化而有力量；也因为同一原因而危险。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Reality (现实; en: reality)** exceeds representation; **Model (模型; en: model)** selects, formalizes, and operationalizes aspects of reality. (现实超出表征；模型选择、形式化并操作化现实的某些方面。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** representation becomes predictive and operational. Models do not only describe the world; they intervene in it. (表征变得预测性和操作性。模型不只是描述世界；它们介入世界。)  
  
### 13. Prediction: The Problem of Future as Governable  
  
`Prediction (预测; la: praedicere; en: prediction)`  
**Definition:** the production of claims about future or unknown states from data, models, patterns, or assumptions. (从数据、模型、模式或假设中产生关于未来或未知状态的主张。)  
**Problem solved:** it makes uncertainty actionable. (它使不确定性变得可行动。)  
**Why needed:** contemporary systems govern by forecasting risk, behavior, demand, disease, crime, credit, attention, and performance. (当代系统通过预测风险、行为、需求、疾病、犯罪、信用、注意力和表现来治理。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing risk scoring, recommendation, policing, medicine, finance, logistics, climate, or AI systems. (当分析风险评分、推荐、警务、医学、金融、物流、气候或 AI 系统时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Prediction is not neutral foresight. A prediction can change the field it predicts. A risk score can affect policing; policing affects arrest data; arrest data affects future risk scores. A recommendation predicts interest; the recommendation changes interest. A credit model predicts repayment; its decision changes opportunity.  
  
This is the feedback problem. Prediction becomes governance when it acts on its object.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Prediction governs when forecasts are used to allocate attention, resources, suspicion, opportunity, or intervention. (当预测被用来分配注意力、资源、怀疑、机会或干预时，预测就成为治理。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Forecast (预报; en: forecast)** estimates future states; **Predictive Governance (预测性治理; en: predictive governance)** acts on persons or populations through forecasts. (预报估计未来状态；预测性治理通过预测对个人或人口采取行动。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** the future becomes a site of present control. Risk replaces guilt, probability replaces event, intervention precedes action. (未来成为当前控制的场所。风险取代罪责，概率取代事件，干预先于行动。)  
  
### 14. Classification: The Problem of Categories That Act  
  
`Classification (分类; la: classis + facere; en: classification)`  
**Definition:** the assignment of persons, objects, events, or data points into categories that structure perception, decision, and action. (把人、对象、事件或数据点分配到分类中，这些分类结构化知觉、决策和行动。)  
**Problem solved:** it makes complexity manageable by sorting cases. (它通过归类案例使复杂性变得可管理。)  
**Why needed:** institutions act through categories: citizen, migrant, risk, eligible, fraudulent, normal, disorder, spam, toxic, qualified, suspicious. (制度通过分类行动：公民、移民、风险、合格、欺诈、正常、障碍、垃圾信息、有毒、合格者、可疑者。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing machine learning, bureaucracy, law, medicine, content moderation, policing, or identity systems. (当分析机器学习、官僚制、法律、医学、内容审核、警务或身份系统时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Classification is never merely mental. It has consequences. A classification can grant treatment, deny credit, trigger investigation, hide speech, rank a worker, identify a disease, or mark a person as risky.  
  
Foucault showed that classification produces objects of knowledge. Contemporary computation intensifies this by making classification scalable, automatic, and constantly updated.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Classification becomes power when categories trigger institutional consequences. (当分类触发制度后果时，分类就成为权力。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Description (描述; en: description)** says what something is; **Classification (分类; en: classification)** places it within a category that governs what can be done with it. (描述说明某物是什么；分类把某物放入支配其可被如何处理的范畴中。)
