**Genealogical shift:** taxonomy becomes automated governance. The category is no longer only conceptual; it is executable. (分类法成为自动化治理。范畴不再只是概念性的；它是可执行的。)  
  
### 15. Automation: The Problem of Delegated Action  
  
`Automation (自动化; el: αὐτόματος; en: automation)`  
**Definition:** the delegation of tasks, decisions, or operations to machines or computational systems. (把任务、决策或操作委托给机器或计算系统。)  
**Problem solved:** it scales action beyond direct human performance. (它使行动超出直接人类执行而得以扩展。)  
**Why needed:** contemporary systems automate production, logistics, moderation, diagnosis, trading, translation, writing, coding, surveillance, and decision support. (当代系统自动化生产、物流、审核、诊断、交易、翻译、写作、编程、监视和决策支持。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing machine action, workflow delegation, decision systems, labor replacement, or automated governance. (当分析机器行动、工作流委托、决策系统、劳动替代或自动化治理时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Automation changes labor and responsibility. If a human acts, responsibility has an identifiable agent. If an automated system acts through designers, data, model, vendor, institution, user, and policy, responsibility diffuses.  
  
Automation also changes skill. It can remove drudgery, but it can also deskill workers, hide judgment, create dependence, and make errors harder to notice.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Automation does not eliminate agency; it redistributes agency across humans, machines, institutions, and procedures. (自动化并不消除行动者性；它在人、机器、制度和程序之间重新分配行动者性。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Mechanization (机械化; en: mechanization)** replaces or assists physical operations; **Automation (自动化; en: automation)** delegates control, decision, or process execution to systems. (机械化替代或辅助物理操作；自动化把控制、决策或过程执行委托给系统。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** labor becomes supervised machine process. The worker may become operator, monitor, exception-handler, trainer, or data producer. (劳动变成被监督的机器过程。劳动者可能成为操作员、监控者、异常处理者、训练者或数据生产者。)  
  
### 16. Human Oversight: The Problem of Responsibility after Automation  
  
`Human Oversight (人类监督; en: human oversight)`  
**Definition:** human review, intervention, correction, or accountability over automated or semi-automated systems. (对自动或半自动系统的人类审查、干预、修正或问责。)  
**Problem solved:** it attempts to preserve judgment and responsibility when action is delegated to machines. (它试图在行动被委托给机器时保留判断和责任。)  
**Why needed:** automated systems can scale errors, misclassify cases, amplify bias, or act without contextual judgment. (自动化系统可能扩大错误、误分类案例、放大偏见或在缺乏语境判断的情况下行动。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing AI governance, content moderation, medical decision support, autonomous systems, hiring tools, or risk scores. (当分析 AI 治理、内容审核、医学决策支持、自动系统、招聘工具或风险评分时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Human oversight is often invoked too easily. A human “in the loop” may be overworked, under-informed, pressured to approve machine outputs, or unable to understand the system. Oversight is meaningful only when the human has time, authority, information, training, and real power to override.  
  
Automation versus human oversight is a tradeoff: automation scales action, while oversight preserves judgment and accountability.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Human oversight is meaningful only when the human can understand, contest, and change the system’s action. (只有当人能够理解、质疑并改变系统行动时，人类监督才有意义。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Human-in-the-Loop (人在回路中; en: human-in-the-loop)** may be procedural presence; **Human Oversight (人类监督; en: human oversight)** requires substantive authority and accountability. (人在回路中可能只是程序性存在；人类监督要求实质性权威与问责。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** responsibility becomes infrastructural. It must be designed into systems, not added as an afterthought. (责任变得基础设施化。它必须被设计进系统，而不是事后附加。)  
  
### 17. Opacity and Explainability: The Problem of Knowing Why  
  
`Opacity (不透明性; en: opacity)`  
**Definition:** the condition in which a system’s internal operation, reasoning, data, objective, or decision path is difficult or impossible to understand. (系统的内部运作、推理、数据、目标或决策路径难以或无法理解的状态。)  
**Problem solved:** it names the gap between system output and human understanding. (它命名系统输出与人类理解之间的裂缝。)  
**Why needed:** complex models, proprietary systems, data pipelines, and institutional secrecy can make decisions hard to contest. (复杂模型、专有系统、数据管道和制度保密会使决策难以被质疑。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing black-box models, bureaucratic secrecy, proprietary algorithms, or complex infrastructures. (当分析黑箱模型、官僚保密、专有算法或复杂基础设施时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
`Explainability (可解释性; en: explainability)`  
**Definition:** the capacity to provide intelligible reasons, mechanisms, or accounts for a system’s output or behavior. (为系统输出或行为提供可理解理由、机制或说明的能力。)  
**Problem solved:** it attempts to make automated decisions understandable and contestable. (它试图使自动化决策可理解且可质疑。)  
**Why needed:** affected persons and responsible institutions need more than outputs; they need reasons, evidence, and accountability. (受影响者和负责制度需要的不只是输出，还需要理由、证据和问责。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing AI systems, medical models, credit scoring, legal decisions, or administrative automation. (当分析 AI 系统、医学模型、信用评分、法律决策或行政自动化时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Explainability is not always the same as understanding. A simplified explanation may be misleading. A technical explanation may be useless to affected persons. A legal explanation may require reasons tied to rights, not merely model features.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Explainability matters because a decision that cannot be understood often cannot be contested. (可解释性重要，因为无法理解的决策往往无法被质疑。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Accuracy (准确性; en: accuracy)** measures performance against a target; **Explainability (可解释性; en: explainability)** concerns intelligible access to how or why outputs are produced. (准确性衡量相对于目标的表现；可解释性关涉对输出如何或为何产生的可理解通达。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** reason-giving becomes a technical and political demand. A system must not only work; it must answer. (给出理由成为技术和政治要求。系统不只要运作；还必须回应。)  
  
### 18. Accountability: The Problem of Answerability  
  
`Accountability (问责性; en: accountability)`  
**Definition:** the condition in which actors, institutions, or systems can be required to justify actions, accept responsibility, repair harm, and submit to oversight. (行动者、制度或系统能够被要求证明行动、承担责任、修复伤害并接受监督的状态。)  
**Problem solved:** it prevents technical systems from diffusing responsibility beyond reach. (它防止技术系统把责任扩散到无法追究的程度。)  
**Why needed:** harms from automated systems often involve many actors: designers, deployers, vendors, data providers, institutions, regulators, and users. (自动化系统造成的伤害常涉及多个行动者：设计者、部署者、供应商、数据提供者、制度、监管者和用户。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing responsibility, audit, liability, governance, appeal, remedy, and institutional design. (当分析责任、审计、责任承担、治理、申诉、救济和制度设计时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Accountability is stronger than transparency. A system may be transparent but still unaccountable if no one can change it, challenge it, or repair its harms. Accountability requires answerability, authority, procedures, evidence, and remedy.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Accountability means that technical power must be answerable to those it affects. (问责性意味着技术权力必须对其影响的人负责。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Transparency (透明性; en: transparency)** makes information visible; **Accountability (问责性; en: accountability)** creates obligations to justify, correct, and repair. (透明性使信息可见；问责性创造证明、修正和修复的义务。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** ethics becomes institutional design. Responsibility must be distributed, documented, enforceable, and revisable. (伦理变成制度设计。责任必须被分配、记录、执行和修正。)  
  
### 19. Platform: The Problem of Mediated Sociality  
  
`Platform (平台; fr: plateforme; en: platform)`  
**Definition:** a digital infrastructure that mediates interactions among users, producers, advertisers, developers, workers, institutions, and data systems. (一种数字基础设施，它中介用户、生产者、广告商、开发者、劳动者、制度和数据系统之间的互动。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains digital systems that do not merely provide services but organize multi-sided social and economic relations. (它解释那些不只是提供服务，而是组织多边社会与经济关系的数字系统。)  
**Why needed:** platforms govern visibility, access, reputation, monetization, moderation, labor, and data extraction. (平台治理可见性、可及性、声誉、变现、审核、劳动和数据提取。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing social media, marketplaces, app stores, ride-hailing, delivery systems, streaming, creator economies, or cloud ecosystems. (当分析社交媒体、市场平台、应用商店、网约车、外卖系统、流媒体、创作者经济或云生态时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
A platform is not just a website or app. It is a governance environment. It sets rules, ranks content, collects data, mediates payments, resolves disputes, enforces policies, shapes incentives, and changes how participants understand themselves.  
  
Platforms are placed near HCI, socio-technical systems, economics, sociology, law, governance, and responsible AI, not merely software architecture.  
  
**Typical sentence:** A platform is infrastructure that becomes social order by mediating interaction and setting the rules of visibility, access, and exchange. (平台是基础设施，它通过中介互动并设定可见性、可及性和交换规则而成为社会秩序。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Application (应用; en: application)** performs a function for users; **Platform (平台; en: platform)** organizes an ecosystem of users, producers, rules, data, and incentives. (应用为用户执行功能；平台组织由用户、生产者、规则、数据和激励构成的生态系统。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** infrastructure becomes market and polity. Platforms govern while presenting themselves as neutral intermediaries. (基础设施成为市场和政治体。平台在自我呈现为中立中介的同时进行治理。)  
  
### 20. Platform Capitalism: The Problem of Extraction through Mediation  
  
`Platform Capitalism (平台资本主义; en: platform capitalism)`  
**Definition:** a form of capitalism in which platforms extract value by mediating interactions, collecting data, controlling access, and organizing markets or labor. (一种资本主义形式，平台通过中介互动、收集数据、控制可及性并组织市场或劳动来榨取价值。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains why digital mediation becomes a business model. (它解释为什么数字中介会成为商业模式。)  
**Why needed:** platforms can profit from network effects, data accumulation, rent extraction, labor coordination, advertising, and dependency. (平台可以从网络效应、数据积累、租金榨取、劳动协调、广告和依赖中获利。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing digital monopolies, app stores, gig work, cloud ecosystems, creator platforms, marketplaces, or data-driven advertising. (当分析数字垄断、应用商店、零工劳动、云生态、创作者平台、市场平台或数据驱动广告时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Platform capitalism often appears as convenience. But convenience is also dependency. A platform becomes powerful when others must pass through it: sellers need marketplace access, creators need visibility, drivers need dispatch, developers need app stores, businesses need cloud infrastructure, advertisers need targeting systems.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Platform capitalism extracts value by becoming the obligatory passage point for interaction, labor, data, and exchange. (平台资本主义通过成为互动、劳动、数据和交换的必经通道来榨取价值。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Industrial Capitalism (工业资本主义; en: industrial capitalism)** extracts value mainly through production and factory labor; **Platform Capitalism (平台资本主义; en: platform capitalism)** extracts value through mediation, data, network effects, and access control. (工业资本主义主要通过生产和工厂劳动榨取价值；平台资本主义通过中介、数据、网络效应和访问控制榨取价值。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** capital moves from owning factories to owning coordination. Control over the interface becomes control over value. (资本从拥有工厂转向拥有协调。控制界面成为控制价值。)  
  
### 21. Surveillance Capitalism: The Problem of Behavioral Extraction  
  
`Surveillance Capitalism (监控资本主义; en: surveillance capitalism)`  
**Definition:** a form of economic accumulation based on extracting behavioral data, predicting or shaping behavior, and monetizing those predictions or interventions. (一种经济积累形式，它基于提取行为数据、预测或塑造行为，并将这些预测或干预货币化。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains why surveillance becomes profitable at scale. (它解释为什么监视在规模化条件下会变得有利可图。)  
**Why needed:** digital systems often collect more behavioral trace than is necessary for immediate service provision. (数字系统常收集超出即时服务所需的行为痕迹。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing targeted advertising, behavioral prediction, personalization, recommendation, smart devices, attention capture, or commercial surveillance. (当分析定向广告、行为预测、个性化、推荐、智能设备、注意力捕获或商业监视时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Surveillance capitalism differs from older surveillance because it is integrated with markets, personalization, advertising, and behavioral modification. The subject is not only watched by the state. The subject is tracked, modeled, targeted, nudged, and monetized by commercial infrastructures.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Surveillance capitalism converts behavioral traces into predictive products and systems of behavioral influence. (监控资本主义把行为痕迹转化为预测产品和行为影响系统。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **State Surveillance (国家监视; en: state surveillance)** watches for security or administrative purposes; **Surveillance Capitalism (监控资本主义; en: surveillance capitalism)** extracts and monetizes behavioral data. (国家监视出于安全或行政目的观察；监控资本主义提取并货币化行为数据。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** attention and behavior become raw material. The subject becomes both consumer and data source. (注意力与行为成为原材料。主体既是消费者，也是数据来源。)  
  
### 22. Attention Economy: The Problem of Captured Awareness  
  
`Attention Economy (注意力经济; en: attention economy)`  
**Definition:** an economic arrangement in which human attention is treated as scarce resource, commodity, and target of competition. (一种经济配置，其中人的注意力被视为稀缺资源、商品和竞争目标。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains why systems are designed to capture, hold, redirect, and monetize attention. (它解释为什么系统被设计为捕获、保持、重定向并货币化注意力。)  
**Why needed:** digital platforms often optimize for engagement, retention, click-through, watch time, and behavioral response. (数字平台常优化参与度、留存、点击率、观看时长和行为反应。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing social media, advertising, recommendation systems, interface design, distraction, outrage, or addiction-like engagement. (当分析社交媒体、广告、推荐系统、界面设计、分心、愤怒或类成瘾参与时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Attention is not only individual focus. It is socially organized. A feed ranks what appears. Notifications interrupt time. Metrics create feedback. Recommendations guide desire. Interface friction or ease shapes behavior.  
  
The attention economy links Lacanian desire, Foucaultian discipline, and platform capitalism. The subject is trained to return, scroll, compare, react, and produce trace.  
  
**Typical sentence:** The attention economy treats awareness as a resource to be captured, allocated, and monetized. (注意力经济把意识注意视为可被捕获、分配和货币化的资源。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Communication (交流; en: communication)** transmits meaning; **Attention Economy (注意力经济; en: attention economy)** organizes the competition for the conditions under which meaning is noticed. (交流传递意义；注意力经济组织对意义得以被注意之条件的竞争。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** subjectivity becomes attention-managed. What appears in consciousness is increasingly shaped by ranking systems. (主体性变得由注意力管理。意识中出现什么越来越受排序系统塑造。)  
  
### 23. Digital Labor: The Problem of Hidden Work in Technical Systems  
  
`Digital Labor (数字劳动; en: digital labor)`  
**Definition:** labor performed through, for, or within digital systems, including platform work, content creation, moderation, data labeling, user activity, and affective engagement. (通过、为了或在数字系统内部执行的劳动，包括平台劳动、内容创作、审核、数据标注、用户活动和情感参与。)  
**Problem solved:** it reveals labor hidden behind automation, participation, convenience, or play. (它揭示隐藏在自动化、参与、便利或娱乐背后的劳动。)  
**Why needed:** digital systems depend on visible and invisible workers: drivers, moderators, annotators, creators, warehouse workers, clickworkers, users, maintainers, and infrastructure laborers. (数字系统依赖可见与不可见劳动者：司机、审核员、标注员、创作者、仓库工人、点击工人、用户、维护者和基础设施劳动者。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing gig work, platform labor, content moderation, data labeling, user-generated value, or AI training pipelines. (当分析零工劳动、平台劳动、内容审核、数据标注、用户生成价值或 AI 训练管道时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Automation often hides labor rather than removing it. An AI system may require labeled data, human feedback, content filtering, infrastructure maintenance, warehouse logistics, energy systems, and moderation work. A platform may call workers “partners” or “creators” while controlling rates, visibility, access, and discipline.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Digital labor names the human work that makes apparently automated systems possible and profitable. (数字劳动命名使看似自动化系统成为可能并有利可图的人类劳动。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Automation (自动化; en: automation)** suggests machine operation; **Digital Labor (数字劳动; en: digital labor)** reveals the human work distributed around that operation. (自动化暗示机器运作；数字劳动揭示围绕这种运作分布的人类劳动。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** social reproduction enters the platform. Hidden labor now includes data cleaning, moderation, annotation, attention, and affect. (社会再生产进入平台。隐藏劳动现在包括数据清洗、审核、标注、注意力和情感。)  
  
### 24. AI Agent: The Problem of Delegated Cognitive Action  
  
`AI Agent (AI 智能体; en: AI agent)`  
**Definition:** an AI system designed to perceive information, plan or select actions, use tools, interact with environments, and pursue goals with some degree of autonomy. (一种 AI 系统，它被设计为感知信息、规划或选择行动、使用工具、同环境互动，并以某种自主程度追求目标。)  
**Problem solved:** it names systems that move beyond passive output generation toward tool-using action. (它命名那些从被动输出生成转向使用工具行动的系统。)  
**Why needed:** contemporary AI increasingly writes, searches, calls tools, updates files, manages workflows, and interacts with external systems. (当代 AI 越来越多地写作、搜索、调用工具、更新文件、管理工作流并同外部系统互动。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing AI systems that act across steps, tools, goals, memory, and environments. (当分析跨步骤、工具、目标、记忆和环境行动的 AI 系统时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
The philosophical problem of AI agents is not only intelligence. It is delegated action. When a system plans, calls tools, sends messages, modifies documents, triggers transactions, or recommends interventions, agency becomes distributed between user, model, tool, designer, institution, and environment.  
  
**Typical sentence:** An AI agent is not merely a text generator; it is a system that can connect representation, planning, tool-use, and action. (AI 智能体不只是文本生成器，而是能够连接表征、规划、工具使用和行动的系统。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Model (模型; en: model)** produces outputs from inputs; **Agent (智能体; en: agent)** acts in an environment according to goals, tools, feedback, or policies. (模型从输入产生输出；智能体根据目标、工具、反馈或策略在环境中行动。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** computation moves from representation to action. The ethical question shifts from “what does the system say?” to “what does the system do?” (计算从表征转向行动。伦理问题从“系统说什么？”转向“系统做什么？”)  
  
### 25. Alignment: The Problem of Machine Goals and Human Values  
  
`Alignment (对齐; en: alignment)`  
**Definition:** the problem of making AI systems act in ways that are compatible with human intentions, values, safety constraints, institutional norms, and legitimate purposes. (使 AI 系统以符合人类意图、价值、安全约束、制度规范和正当目的的方式行动的问题。)  
**Problem solved:** it addresses the gap between specified objectives and desirable behavior. (它处理被规定目标与可欲行为之间的差距。)  
**Why needed:** systems can optimize proxies, exploit loopholes, misgeneralize, produce harmful outputs, or act unpredictably in new contexts. (系统可能优化代理指标、利用漏洞、错误泛化、产生有害输出，或在新语境中不可预测地行动。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing AI safety, model behavior, reward design, human feedback, governance, or value specification. (当分析 AI 安全、模型行为、奖励设计、人类反馈、治理或价值规定时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Alignment is not only a technical problem. It is philosophical, political, and institutional. Whose values? Which context? What conflicts? What tradeoffs? What accountability? What happens when users, firms, states, and affected communities disagree?  
  
A narrow alignment problem asks whether a model follows the developer’s intended objective. A broader alignment problem asks whether the system’s behavior is justifiable within a social world of rights, risks, plural values, and power asymmetries.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Alignment asks whether an AI system’s behavior remains answerable to legitimate human purposes rather than merely optimized objectives. (对齐追问 AI 系统的行为是否仍能回应正当人类目的，而不只是优化目标函数。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Optimization (优化; en: optimization)** maximizes or minimizes an objective; **Alignment (对齐; en: alignment)** asks whether the objective and resulting behavior are normatively acceptable. (优化最大化或最小化目标；对齐追问目标及其产生的行为是否在规范上可接受。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** ethics enters system design at the level of objective, representation, feedback, and deployment. (伦理进入系统设计的目标、表征、反馈和部署层面。)  
  
### 26. Posthuman: The Problem of Human after Technics  
  
`Posthuman (后人类; en: posthuman)`  
**Definition:** a concept naming forms of subjectivity, embodiment, agency, and life that exceed the classical humanist image of the autonomous rational individual. (一个命名超出古典人文主义自主理性个体图像的主体性、具身性、行动者性和生命形式的概念。)  
**Problem solved:** it challenges the assumption that “the human” is fixed, pure, self-contained, and separate from technology, animals, ecology, and machines. (它挑战“人”是固定、纯粹、自足并同技术、动物、生态和机器分离的假设。)  
**Why needed:** contemporary life is technologically mediated, biologically entangled, environmentally dependent, and increasingly machine-interactive. (当代生活被技术中介、同生物纠缠、依赖环境，并越来越同机器互动。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing human-machine systems, biotechnology, AI, cyborgs, ecological dependency, disability technology, or anti-humanist critique. (当分析人机系统、生物技术、AI、赛博格、生态依赖、残障技术或反人文主义批判时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Posthuman theory does not necessarily mean humans are obsolete. It means the old model of the human as sovereign, rational, disembodied, and separate from the world is no longer adequate.  
  
The posthuman subject is distributed: through devices, data, prostheses, networks, environments, microbes, infrastructures, and nonhuman agents.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Posthuman theory asks what becomes of the human when agency, embodiment, and cognition are distributed across technical and ecological systems. (后人类理论追问当行动者性、具身性和认知分布在人类、技术和生态系统之间时，“人”会变成什么。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Humanism (人文主义; la: humanitas)** often centers human reason and dignity; **Posthumanism (后人类主义; en: posthumanism)** questions the boundaries and privileges of that human figure. (人文主义常以人的理性和尊严为中心；后人类主义质疑该人类形象的边界和特权。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** the subject becomes distributed. The human is no longer the unquestioned center of ontology, ethics, or politics. (主体变得分布化。人不再是本体论、伦理或政治的未经质疑中心。)  
  
### 27. Cyborg: The Problem of Hybrid Body  
  
`Cyborg (赛博格; en: cybernetic organism)`  
**Definition:** a hybrid of organism and machine, often used critically to rethink embodiment, identity, gender, labor, and technology. (有机体与机器的混合体，常被批判性地用于重思具身性、身份、性别、劳动和技术。)  
**Problem solved:** it breaks the binary between natural body and artificial machine. (它打破自然身体与人工机器之间的二元对立。)  
**Why needed:** modern bodies are already technically mediated through medicine, prosthetics, devices, networks, implants, hormones, screens, and data systems. (现代身体已经通过医学、义肢、设备、网络、植入物、激素、屏幕和数据系统被技术中介。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing feminist technoscience, prosthetics, disability, trans embodiment, biohacking, wearable devices, or human-machine identity. (当分析女性主义技术科学、义肢、残障、跨性别具身性、生物黑客、可穿戴设备或人机身份时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
The cyborg is not only science fiction. It is a political figure. It refuses purity: pure nature, pure gender, pure body, pure machine, pure origin. This makes it useful for feminist and queer theory.  
  
**Typical sentence:** The cyborg shows that bodies are not sealed natural origins but hybrid technical formations. (赛博格显示身体不是封闭的自然起源，而是混合的技术形成物。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Natural Body (自然身体; en: natural body)** imagines the body before technology; **Cyborg Body (赛博格身体; en: cyborg body)** treats the body as technically mediated and hybrid. (自然身体想象技术之前的身体；赛博格身体把身体视为被技术中介且混合的存在。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** embodiment becomes technopolitical. The body is not opposed to technology; it is partly made through technology. (具身性变得技术政治化。身体不与技术对立；身体部分地通过技术被制造。)  
  
### 28. Anthropocene: The Problem of Human Geological Force  
  
`Anthropocene (人类世; el: ἄνθρωπος + καινός; en: Anthropocene)`  
**Definition:** a proposed epochal concept naming the period in which human activity has become a geological and planetary force. (一个拟议的时代概念，命名人类活动成为地质和行星力量的时期。)  
**Problem solved:** it shows that human history and Earth history can no longer be cleanly separated. (它显示人类史与地球史已不能被干净地区分。)  
**Why needed:** industrial activity, fossil fuel use, extraction, agriculture, urbanization, mass extinction, pollution, and climate change transform planetary systems. (工业活动、化石燃料使用、榨取、农业、城市化、大灭绝、污染和气候变化转化行星系统。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing climate crisis, ecological responsibility, planetary boundaries, environmental politics, extraction, or species-level agency. (当分析气候危机、生态责任、行星边界、环境政治、榨取或物种层面行动者性时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
The Anthropocene is conceptually powerful but politically risky. It says “humanity” has become geological force. But not all humans contributed equally. Industrial capitalism, colonial extraction, fossil capital, military systems, wealthy states, and corporate infrastructures matter more than abstract humanity.  
  
This is why many theorists prefer or supplement it with terms such as **Capitalocene (资本世; en: Capitalocene)**, which emphasizes capitalism’s role, or **Plantationocene (种植园世; en: Plantationocene)**, which emphasizes plantation, slavery, monoculture, and colonial ecology.  
  
**Typical sentence:** The Anthropocene names the planetary consequences of human activity, but it must be corrected by asking which humans, institutions, and economies caused those consequences. (人类世命名人类活动的行星后果，但必须通过追问哪些人、制度和经济导致这些后果来修正。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Anthropocene (人类世; en: Anthropocene)** centers humanity as geological force; **Capitalocene (资本世; en: Capitalocene)** centers capital accumulation and fossil extraction. (人类世以人类作为地质力量为中心；资本世以资本积累和化石榨取为中心。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** history becomes planetary. Ethics and politics must account for atmospheres, oceans, species, extraction, waste, and future generations. (历史变得行星化。伦理与政治必须说明大气、海洋、物种、榨取、废弃物和未来世代。)  
  
### 29. Extraction: The Problem of Taking from Worlds  
  
`Extraction (榨取/抽取; la: extrahere; en: extraction)`  
**Definition:** the removal of value, matter, energy, labor, data, or attention from bodies, communities, environments, or systems for accumulation elsewhere. (从身体、共同体、环境或系统中移出价值、物质、能源、劳动、数据或注意力，并在别处积累。)  
**Problem solved:** it connects colonialism, capitalism, datafication, energy systems, and ecological crisis. (它把殖民主义、资本主义、数据化、能源系统和生态危机连接起来。)  
**Why needed:** contemporary systems extract not only minerals and labor, but also data, affect, attention, and predictive value. (当代系统不仅榨取矿物和劳动，也榨取数据、情感、注意力和预测价值。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing mining, fossil fuels, colonial resource flows, platform data, labor exploitation, attention capture, or ecological damage. (当分析采矿、化石燃料、殖民资源流动、平台数据、劳动剥削、注意力捕获或生态损害时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Extraction is a bridge concept. Marx helps analyze labor extraction. Postcolonial theory helps analyze resource extraction. Feminism helps analyze reproductive and affective labor extraction. Platform theory helps analyze data and attention extraction. Environmental humanities help analyze planetary extraction.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Extraction names the movement by which value is taken from one body, community, or ecology and accumulated elsewhere. (榨取命名价值从一个身体、共同体或生态中被取出并在别处积累的运动。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Production (生产; la: productio)** emphasizes making; **Extraction (榨取; en: extraction)** emphasizes taking, depletion, and transfer. (生产强调制造；榨取强调取出、耗竭和转移。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** critique moves from factory to planet and platform. Value extraction now includes labor, land, data, attention, and future livability. (批判从工厂扩展到行星和平台。价值榨取现在包括劳动、土地、数据、注意力和未来宜居性。)  
  
### 30. Planetary Crisis: The Problem of Shared but Unequal Vulnerability  
  
`Planetary Crisis (行星危机; en: planetary crisis)`  
**Definition:** the interlinked crisis of climate, biodiversity, extraction, pollution, water, food systems, energy, displacement, and unequal vulnerability at planetary scale. (气候、生物多样性、榨取、污染、水、食物系统、能源、流离失所和不平等脆弱性在行星尺度上相互连接的危机。)  
**Problem solved:** it prevents ecological crisis from being reduced to one issue such as carbon alone. (它防止生态危机被化约为碳等单一问题。)  
**Why needed:** ecological harm is distributed unequally across class, race, empire, geography, gender, generation, and species. (生态伤害按阶级、种族、帝国、地理、性别、世代和物种不平等分布。)  
**How to use:** use it when analyzing climate justice, environmental racism, extraction zones, migration, disaster, food systems, energy transition, or intergenerational ethics. (当分析气候正义、环境种族主义、榨取区、迁移、灾害、食物系统、能源转型或代际伦理时，应使用这一概念。)  
  
Planetary crisis is not a “nature” problem outside society. It is produced through infrastructures, economies, colonial histories, energy regimes, consumption systems, military systems, agriculture, and technology.  
  
This is where the entire tutorial converges. Metaphysics asks what kind of world is being presupposed. Ethics asks who is responsible. Political theory asks who decides. Postcolonial theory asks who pays. Feminism asks who cares. Technology critique asks what systems mediate action. Pragmatism asks what consequences follow.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Planetary crisis is not humanity facing nature from outside; it is a crisis of the systems through which humans inhabit Earth. (行星危机不是人类从外部面对自然，而是人类居住地球的系统本身发生危机。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Environmental Problem (环境问题; en: environmental problem)** may sound local or technical; **Planetary Crisis (行星危机; en: planetary crisis)** names interdependent Earth-system, social, economic, and political breakdown. (环境问题听起来可能是局部或技术性的；行星危机命名地球系统、社会、经济和政治的相互依赖性崩解。)  
  
**Genealogical shift:** politics becomes ecological and temporal. It must include nonhumans, infrastructures, future generations, and irreversible damage. (政治变得生态化和时间化。它必须纳入非人类、基础设施、未来世代和不可逆伤害。)  
  
### 31. The Contemporary Critical Diagnostic Method  
  
Contemporary critical analysis should not become a vague complaint that technology is bad. The method is sharper.  
  
A strong analysis asks:  
  
**What representation makes this system possible?**  
(什么表征使这个系统成为可能？)  
  
**What does the system measure, and what does it ignore?**  
(系统测量什么，又忽略什么？)  
  
**What data is extracted, from whom, under what consent or dependency?**  
(什么数据从谁那里被提取，在什么同意或依赖条件下被提取？)  
  
**What model or algorithm acts on the data?**  
(什么模型或算法作用于这些数据？)  
  
**What institution acts on the output?**  
(什么制度根据输出采取行动？)  
  
**Who can understand, contest, appeal, or repair the decision?**  
(谁能够理解、质疑、申诉或修复该决策？)  
  
**What labor, energy, infrastructure, and extraction are hidden?**  
(什么劳动、能源、基础设施和榨取被隐藏？)  
  
**What form of life does the system train?**  
(该系统训练出什么生活形式？)  
  
**Typical sentence:** Contemporary critical reading follows the chain from representation to data, from data to model, from model to decision, from decision to institution, and from institution to form of life. (当代批判阅读追踪从表征到数据、从数据到模型、从模型到决策、从决策到制度、从制度到生活形式的链条。)  
  
### 32. The Tool-Map of Contemporary Critical Vocabulary  
  
Use contemporary critical vocabulary diagnostically. The core question is usually not only “does the technology work?” but “what world does it build by working?”  
  
**If the text analyzes technology as world-ordering**, look for **Technology (技术; de: Technik)**, **Technics (技术性; fr: technique)**, and **Enframing (集置; de: Gestell)**.  
(如果文本把技术分析为世界订置，应寻找技术、技术性和集置问题。)  
  
**If the text analyzes hidden background systems**, look for **Infrastructure (基础设施; en: infrastructure)**.  
(如果文本分析隐藏的背景系统，应寻找基础设施问题。)  
  
**If the text analyzes representation and records**, look for **Data (数据; la: datum)**, **Datafication (数据化; en: datafication)**, **Database (数据库; en: database)**, and **Metadata (元数据; en: metadata)**.  
(如果文本分析表征和记录，应寻找数据、数据化、数据库和元数据问题。)  
  
**If the text analyzes computational procedure**, look for **Algorithm (算法; en: algorithm)** and **Algorithmic Governance (算法治理; en: algorithmic governance)**.  
(如果文本分析计算程序，应寻找算法和算法治理问题。)  
  
**If the text analyzes simplified representations**, look for **Model (模型; en: model)**, **Prediction (预测; en: prediction)**, and **Classification (分类; en: classification)**.  
(如果文本分析简化表征，应寻找模型、预测和分类问题。)  
  
**If the text analyzes machine delegation**, look for **Automation (自动化; en: automation)**, **Human Oversight (人类监督; en: human oversight)**, and **Accountability (问责性; en: accountability)**.  
(如果文本分析机器委托，应寻找自动化、人类监督和问责性问题。)  
  
**If the text analyzes black-box decisions**, look for **Opacity (不透明性; en: opacity)** and **Explainability (可解释性; en: explainability)**.  
(如果文本分析黑箱决策，应寻找不透明性和可解释性问题。)  
  
**If the text analyzes digital mediation**, look for **Platform (平台; en: platform)**, **Platform Capitalism (平台资本主义; en: platform capitalism)**, and **Surveillance Capitalism (监控资本主义; en: surveillance capitalism)**.  
(如果文本分析数字中介，应寻找平台、平台资本主义和监控资本主义问题。)  
  
**If the text analyzes attention and participation**, look for **Attention Economy (注意力经济; en: attention economy)** and **Digital Labor (数字劳动; en: digital labor)**.  
(如果文本分析注意力和参与，应寻找注意力经济和数字劳动问题。)  
  
**If the text analyzes autonomous AI systems**, look for **AI Agent (AI 智能体; en: AI agent)** and **Alignment (对齐; en: alignment)**.  
(如果文本分析自主 AI 系统，应寻找 AI 智能体和对齐问题。)  
  
**If the text questions the human-machine boundary**, look for **Posthuman (后人类; en: posthuman)** and **Cyborg (赛博格; en: cyborg)**.  
(如果文本质疑人机边界，应寻找后人类和赛博格问题。)  
  
**If the text analyzes ecological crisis**, look for **Anthropocene (人类世; en: Anthropocene)**, **Capitalocene (资本世; en: Capitalocene)**, **Extraction (榨取; en: extraction)**, and **Planetary Crisis (行星危机; en: planetary crisis)**.  
(如果文本分析生态危机，应寻找人类世、资本世、榨取和行星危机问题。)  
  
### 33. The Genealogical Point of Part 19  
  
Contemporary critical vocabulary transforms the philosophical language of technology and world. Greek philosophy treated **technē (技艺; el: τέχνη)** as craft and know-how. Modern philosophy often treated technology as instrument. Heidegger showed that modern technology is a mode of revealing. Critical Theory diagnosed instrumental reason. Marx analyzed capital and extraction. Foucault showed how knowledge makes subjects and populations governable. Derrida showed how archive, trace, signature, and iterability structure authority. Feminism revealed hidden labor and embodied vulnerability. Postcolonial theory revealed empire, extraction, and racial hierarchy. Pragmatism asked what concepts do in practice.  
  
Contemporary critical theory adds:  
  
**Technical systems do not merely serve forms of life; they produce forms of life.**  
(技术系统不只是服务生活形式；它们生产生活形式。)  
  
The guiding thesis is:  
  
**Contemporary critical vocabulary turns technology into a problem of world-production: to understand a technical system is to ask what representation it imposes, what data it extracts, what model it uses, what behavior it predicts, what action it automates, what labor and infrastructure it hides, what subject it produces, and what ecological or planetary cost it displaces.**  
(当代批判词汇把技术转化为世界生产问题：理解一个技术系统，就是追问它强加什么表征，提取什么数据，使用什么模型，预测什么行为，自动化什么行动，隐藏什么劳动和基础设施，生产什么主体，以及转移什么生态或行星成本。)  
  
This grammar does not reject technology. It rejects technological innocence. It asks for technical systems to be interpreted as social, political, economic, epistemic, and ecological formations.  
  
The contemporary critical question remains one of the strongest tools for philosophical reading:  
  
**What world must be represented, extracted, optimized, automated, and made disposable for this technical system to appear efficient, intelligent, and inevitable?**  
(为了使这个技术系统显得高效、智能且不可避免，什么世界必须被表征、榨取、优化、自动化并变得可抛弃？)  
  
## Part 20. Methodological Synthesis: Genealogy, Diagnosis, Use  
  
This final methodological chapter explains how to use the previous vocabulary as a working instrument. The point is not to memorize terms as labels. The point is to ask what each term is designed to do. A philosophical concept is not a decorative word. It is a tool that solves a specific problem, reveals a specific structure, blocks a specific confusion, or opens a specific mode of reading.  
  
The central question is:  
  
**How should philosophical vocabulary be used as a diagnostic system rather than as a list of terms?**  
(哲学词汇如何应当作为诊断系统来使用，而不是作为术语清单？)  
  
The central vocabulary is **Concept**, **Problematic**, **Genealogy**, **Historicity**, **Critique**, **Diagnosis**, **Interpretation**, **Structure**, **Discourse**, **Symptom**, **Deconstruction**, **Use**, **Form of Life**, **Normativity**, **Translation**, and **Conceptual Transfer**.  
  
The operational function of this chapter is exact: use this final framework when the problem is **how to read, compare, translate, and deploy philosophical concepts across historical periods, languages, disciplines, and political contexts**.  
(当问题是如何跨历史时期、语言、学科和政治语境阅读、比较、翻译和使用哲学概念时，应使用这一最终框架。)  
  
### 1. The Core Rule: A Concept Is a Tool for a Problem  
  
`Concept (概念; la: conceptus; de: Begriff; fr: concept)`  
**Definition:** a structured intellectual tool used to grasp, distinguish, diagnose, or transform a problem. (一种结构化的思想工具，用来把握、区分、诊断或转化一个问题。)  
**Problem solved:** it prevents philosophical vocabulary from becoming empty terminology. (它防止哲学词汇变成空洞术语。)  
**Why needed:** a concept has philosophical value only when it does work. (一个概念只有在发挥作用时才具有哲学价值。)  
**How to use:** ask what problem the concept was invented or mobilized to solve. (应追问这个概念被发明或动员出来是为了解决什么问题。)  
  
A concept should never be introduced merely by saying what it “means.” It must also be asked what it does. **Being / What-is (存在/所是者; el: τὸ εἶναι / τὸ ὄν)** answers the problem of what it means for anything to be. **Substance (实体; la: substantia)** answers the problem of what remains stable through change. **Subject (主体; la: subiectum; de: Subjekt)** answers the problem of who knows, acts, or bears experience. **Power/Knowledge (权力/知识; fr: savoir-pouvoir; en: power/knowledge)** answers the problem of how truth and domination are historically joined. **Performativity (表演性; en: performativity)** answers the problem of how repeated acts produce identity-effects.  
  
A weak reading says: “This text uses the term power.”  
(弱阅读说：这个文本使用了“权力”这个词。)  
  
A strong reading says: “This text uses **Power (权力; fr: pouvoir)** to move analysis from sovereign command to productive formation of bodies, norms, and subjects.”  
(强阅读说：这个文本使用“权力”把分析从主权命令转向身体、规范和主体的生产性形成。)  
  
**Typical sentence:** A concept becomes philosophical when it reorganizes a problem, not when it merely names a topic.  
(一个概念只有在重组问题时才成为哲学性的，而不只是命名一个主题。)  
  
### 2. Problematic: The Hidden Question-System  
  
`Problematic (问题域; fr: problématique; en: problematic)`  
**Definition:** the structured field of questions, assumptions, tensions, and possible answers within which a concept becomes meaningful. (一个由问题、预设、张力和可能答案构成的结构化场域，概念在其中变得有意义。)  
**Problem solved:** it prevents concepts from being read in isolation. (它防止概念被孤立阅读。)  
**Why needed:** every major concept belongs to a field of pressure. (每个重要概念都属于一个压力场。)  
**How to use:** reconstruct the problem-field that made the concept necessary. (应重构使该概念成为必要的问题场。)  
  
The word **freedom** does not always solve the same problem. In **Kant**, **Freedom (自由; de: Freiheit)** solves the problem of moral autonomy under rational law. In **Hegel**, it solves the problem of recognition and social actualization. In **Marx**, it is blocked by material exploitation and alienated labor. In **Sartre**, it names radical responsibility under existence. In **Foucault**, it appears inside practices of power and self-formation. In feminist theory, it must be rethought through embodiment, dependence, care, and bodily autonomy.  
  
The same term changes because the problematic changes.  
  
**Typical sentence:** To understand a concept, first identify the problematic that makes the concept necessary.  
(理解一个概念，首先要识别使该概念成为必要的问题域。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Topic (主题; en: topic)** is what a text is about; **Problematic (问题域; fr: problématique)** is the structured question-system that gives the topic theoretical force.  
(主题是文本谈论的对象；问题域是赋予该对象理论力量的结构化问题系统。)  
  
### 3. Genealogy: The History of Conceptual Formation  
  
`Genealogy (谱系学; de: Genealogie; fr: généalogie)`  
**Definition:** a historical-critical method that traces how concepts, norms, truths, and subjects are formed through contingent struggles, exclusions, institutions, and practices. (一种历史批判方法，追踪概念、规范、真理和主体如何通过偶然斗争、排除、制度和实践形成。)  
**Problem solved:** it breaks the illusion that present concepts are natural, timeless, or necessary. (它打破当前概念是自然的、永恒的或必然的幻觉。)  
**Why needed:** philosophical vocabulary carries historical sediment. (哲学词汇携带历史沉积。)  
**How to use:** ask what earlier meanings, conflicts, translations, and institutional uses are buried inside the present concept. (应追问当前概念内部埋藏着哪些早期意义、冲突、翻译和制度使用。)  
  
**Usage layers:**  
1. **Nietzschean use (尼采式用法):** **genealogy** investigates the historical emergence of values, morals, ideals, and concepts by tracing struggle, reversal, resentment, interpretation, and power. (在尼采那里，谱系学通过追踪斗争、反转、怨恨、解释和力量来研究价值、道德、理想和概念的历史生成。)  
  
2. **Foucaultian reception use (福柯式接受史用法):** in Foucault, genealogy analyzes the contingent formation of practices, bodies, institutions, subjects, and regimes of truth. (在福柯那里，谱系学分析实践、身体、制度、主体和真理体制的偶然形成。)  
  
3. **Contemporary transferable use (当代理论泛用法):** in social theory, legal theory, critical race theory, gender studies, and media theory, genealogy may trace how something now treated as natural, neutral, or necessary was historically produced. (在社会理论、法理论、批判种族理论、性别研究和媒介理论中，谱系学可追踪某种现在被视为自然、中立或必然之物如何在历史中被生产出来。)  
  
**Transfer rule:** use **genealogy** when the task is not to find timeless essence, but to reconstruct contingent formation. (转用规则：当任务不是寻找永恒本质，而是重建偶然形成过程时，才使用 genealogy。)  
  
**Misuse warning:** genealogy is not ordinary chronology. It is a critical history of formation, value, power, and contingency. (Genealogy 不是普通年代史，而是关于形成、价值、权力和偶然性的批判历史。)  
  
Genealogy does not merely ask where a word came from. Etymology alone is not enough. Genealogy asks how a concept became authoritative, what it displaced, what institutions used it, what bodies it classified, what exclusions it required, and what possibilities it opened or closed.  
  
For example, **Subject (主体; la: subiectum)** originally carries the sense of what lies beneath or is subjected. In modern philosophy it becomes the knowing and acting center. In political theory it can mean one subjected to sovereign power. In Foucault and Butler, subjectivity is both agency and subjection. The concept’s history is not linear. It is a field of reversals.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Genealogy asks how a concept became necessary, who benefited from that necessity, and what alternatives were excluded.  
(谱系学追问一个概念如何变得必要，谁从这种必要性中受益，以及哪些替代可能被排除。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **History of Ideas (观念史; en: history of ideas)** may trace intellectual development; **Genealogy (谱系学; fr: généalogie)** traces contingent formation through power, struggle, exclusion, and practice.  
(观念史可以追踪思想发展；谱系学追踪观念如何通过权力、斗争、排除和实践偶然形成。)  
  
### 4. Historicity: Concepts Change because Problems Change  
  
`Historicity (历史性; de: Geschichtlichkeit; fr: historicité)`  
**Definition:** the condition that concepts, subjects, meanings, and practices are historically formed and historically transformable. (概念、主体、意义和实践都在历史中形成，并且能够在历史中转化的条件。)  
**Problem solved:** it prevents anachronistic reading. (它防止时代错置式阅读。)  
**Why needed:** a concept used by **Aristotle**, **Aquinas**, **Kant**, **Hegel**, **Marx**, **Heidegger**, **Foucault**, and **Butler** cannot be assumed to have one stable function. (亚里士多德、阿奎那、康德、黑格尔、马克思、海德格尔、福柯和巴特勒使用的同一概念不能被假设具有同一稳定功能。)  
**How to use:** locate the concept inside its historical problem, not only inside a dictionary definition. (应把概念放入其历史问题中，而不只是放入词典定义中。)  
  
Historicity is why translation matters. **Logos (逻各斯; el: λόγος)** is not simply “reason.” It can mean speech, account, measure, order, argument, relation, and intelligibility. **Substantia (实体; la: substantia)** is not identical with Greek **ousia (本质/实体; el: οὐσία)**, even when translated into the same modern word. **Geist (精神; de: Geist)** is not simply mind, spirit, or culture, but a historical-conceptual node in German philosophy.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Historicity means that a concept’s meaning is inseparable from the historical problem it answers.  
(历史性意味着一个概念的意义不能脱离它所回应的历史问题。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Chronology (年代顺序; en: chronology)** orders events in time; **Historicity (历史性; de: Geschichtlichkeit)** names the historical constitution of meaning itself.  
(年代顺序按时间排列事件；历史性命名意义本身的历史构成。)  
  
### 5. Interpretation: Recovering Meaning within Horizon  
  
`Interpretation (解释; la: interpretatio; de: Auslegung; fr: interprétation)`  
**Definition:** the act of making sense of a text, action, sign, practice, or event within a horizon of meaning. (在意义视域中理解文本、行动、符号、实践或事件的行动。)  
**Problem solved:** it prevents reading from being reduced to mere extraction of information. (它防止阅读被化约为单纯提取信息。)  
**Why needed:** philosophical texts say things within traditions, genres, questions, and assumptions. (哲学文本总是在传统、文类、问题和预设中说话。)  
**How to use:** ask what the text is trying to make intelligible, against what background, and for what audience. (应追问文本试图使什么变得可理解，在什么背景下，并面向什么读者。)  
  
Hermeneutic reading asks for the whole and the parts. A sentence means through a paragraph, a paragraph through an argument, an argument through a tradition, a tradition through historical life. This does not make interpretation arbitrary. It makes it disciplined by context, textual evidence, and conceptual coherence.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Interpretation reconstructs the horizon in which a text’s claims become intelligible.  
(解释重构文本主张得以成为可理解之物的视域。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Explanation (解释/说明; en: explanation)** may identify causes or mechanisms; **Interpretation (解释; de: Auslegung)** reconstructs meaning within a horizon.  
(说明可以识别原因或机制；解释则重构视域中的意义。)  
  
### 6. Critique: Exposing Conditions and Limits  
  
`Critique (批判; el: κρίνειν; de: Kritik; fr: critique)`  
**Definition:** the examination of the conditions, limits, contradictions, and consequences of a claim, system, practice, or form of reason. (对一个主张、系统、实践或理性形式的条件、限度、矛盾和后果的审查。)  
**Problem solved:** it prevents thought from accepting its own authority too quickly. (它防止思想过快接受自身权威。)  
**Why needed:** every claim has conditions, limits, exclusions, and effects. (每个主张都有条件、限度、排除和效果。)  
**How to use:** ask what makes the claim possible, where it fails, what it excludes, and what it does. (应追问该主张何以可能、在哪里失败、排除什么、产生什么效果。)  
  
Critique has several historical forms. **Kantian critique** asks the conditions and limits of possible knowledge. **Marxian critique** asks how social forms conceal labor, exploitation, and class relation. **Nietzschean critique** asks what drives, values, and power relations hide beneath morality. **Foucauldian critique** asks how truth, norms, and subjects are historically produced. **Feminist critique** asks whose body and labor were excluded from the universal. **Postcolonial critique** asks what empire and race were forgotten.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Critique does not merely reject; it asks what conditions make a claim possible and what limits that claim must not see.  
(批判并不只是拒绝；它追问一个主张何以可能，以及该主张不能看见什么限度。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Objection (反对; en: objection)** disputes a claim; **Critique (批判; de: Kritik)** examines the claim’s conditions, structure, and effects.  
(反对驳斥一个主张；批判审查该主张的条件、结构和效果。)  
  
### 7. Diagnosis: Naming the Structure of a Problem  
  
`Diagnosis (诊断; el: διάγνωσις; en: diagnosis)`  
**Definition:** the analytic act of identifying the underlying structure, cause, tension, or pattern that makes a problem intelligible. (识别使一个问题成为可理解之物的底层结构、原因、张力或模式的分析行动。)  
**Problem solved:** it turns scattered symptoms into a structured problem. (它把分散症状转化为结构化问题。)  
**Why needed:** philosophy often deals not with isolated errors but with patterned confusions, contradictions, and formations. (哲学处理的常不是孤立错误，而是模式化混乱、矛盾和形成物。)  
**How to use:** ask what kind of problem is present: metaphysical, epistemological, ethical, political, linguistic, psychoanalytic, technological, or colonial. (应追问当前是什么类型的问题：形而上学的、认识论的、伦理的、政治的、语言的、精神分析的、技术的或殖民的。)  
  
Diagnosis is the bridge between vocabulary and use. The same object can be diagnosed differently.  
  
A prison can be read as a legal institution, a disciplinary apparatus, a racial technology, a capitalist labor system, a site of state violence, a moral symbol, a database, or a spatial form. The correct reading depends on the question. A strong reader does not use every tool at once. A strong reader selects the tool that best diagnoses the problem.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Diagnosis asks what structure produces the visible problem.  
(诊断追问什么结构生产了可见问题。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Description (描述; en: description)** records what appears; **Diagnosis (诊断; en: diagnosis)** identifies the structure that makes the appearance intelligible.  
(描述记录显现之物；诊断识别使显现成为可理解之物的结构。)  
  
### 8. Structure: Looking for Relations, Not Isolated Objects  
  
`Structure (结构; la: structura; fr: structure)`  
**Definition:** a system of relations in which elements receive meaning, function, or force from their positions. (一种关系系统，其中元素从其位置获得意义、功能或力量。)  
**Problem solved:** it prevents analysis from treating elements as self-contained. (它防止分析把元素视为自足对象。)  
**Why needed:** concepts, identities, signs, laws, institutions, and desires work by relation. (概念、身份、符号、法律、制度和欲望都通过关系运作。)  
**How to use:** ask what relations, oppositions, positions, and rules organize the object. (应追问什么关系、对立、位置和规则组织了该对象。)  
  
Structural reading is useful when meaning depends on oppositions: legal/illegal, normal/abnormal, civilized/barbaric, male/female, human/animal, citizen/foreigner, natural/artificial. The question is not only what each term means. The question is how the pair organizes a field.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Structural analysis asks how relations produce meaning before individual intention appears.  
(结构分析追问在个体意图出现之前，关系如何生产意义。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Element (元素; la: elementum)** is an individual unit; **Structure (结构; fr: structure)** is the relation-system that gives units their function.  
(元素是单个单位；结构是赋予单位功能的关系系统。)  
  
### 9. Discourse: Looking for Rules of Sayability  
  
`Discourse (话语; la: discursus; fr: discours)`  
**Definition:** a historically organized field of statements, rules, institutions, categories, and subject-positions that determines what can be said, known, and recognized. (一种历史组织起来的陈述、规则、制度、分类和主体位置场域，它决定什么能够被说、被知和被承认。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains why truth is not only proposition but also institutional formation. (它解释为什么真理不只是命题，也是制度形成物。)  
**Why needed:** fields such as medicine, law, sexuality, race, security, and education produce objects and subjects through rules of knowledge. (医学、法律、性、种族、安全和教育等领域通过知识规则生产对象和主体。)  
**How to use:** ask what can be said, who can say it, what counts as evidence, and what subject-position is produced. (应追问什么能够被说、谁能够说、什么算作证据，以及什么主体位置被生产出来。)  
  
A discourse is not simply conversation. It is the field that allows certain statements to count as truth. A psychiatric diagnosis, legal category, school grade, immigration risk score, or medical chart is not merely language. It is language connected to authority, institution, classification, and intervention.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Discourse analysis asks what rules make certain statements count as knowledge.  
(话语分析追问什么规则使某些陈述能够算作知识。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Speech (言说; en: speech)** is an utterance; **Discourse (话语; fr: discours)** is the historical field that gives utterances authority and function.  
(言说是发话；话语是赋予发话以权威和功能的历史场域。)  
  
### 10. Symptom: Reading What the Text Cannot Say Directly  
  
`Symptom (症状; el: σύμπτωμα; de: Symptom; fr: symptôme)`  
**Definition:** a formation in which a hidden conflict, contradiction, repression, or structural tension appears indirectly. (隐藏冲突、矛盾、压抑或结构张力以间接形式出现的形成物。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains why meaning may appear through failure, repetition, excess, silence, or contradiction. (它解释为什么意义可能通过失败、重复、过剩、沉默或矛盾出现。)  
**Why needed:** texts and institutions often reveal themselves most clearly where they malfunction. (文本和制度常在失灵之处最清楚地暴露自身。)  
**How to use:** ask what contradiction returns indirectly through the surface. (应追问什么矛盾通过表面间接返回。)  
  
A political speech that repeatedly insists on unity may symptomatically reveal division. A legal system that constantly invokes neutrality may reveal anxiety about bias. A colonial archive that classifies everything may reveal fear of the ungovernable. A personal narrative that avoids one event may make that event structurally central through omission.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Symptomatic reading asks what the text reveals by failing to say it directly.  
(症状性阅读追问文本通过不能直接说出而揭示了什么。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Sign (符号; fr: signe)** signifies within a system; **Symptom (症状; fr: symptôme)** signifies through conflict, repression, or contradiction.  
(符号在系统中表意；症状通过冲突、压抑或矛盾表意。)  
  
### 11. Deconstruction: Reading the Hierarchy’s Dependence  
  
`Deconstruction (解构; fr: déconstruction)`  
**Definition:** a reading practice that shows how a conceptual hierarchy depends on what it subordinates, excludes, or treats as secondary. (一种阅读实践，显示概念等级如何依赖其贬低、排除或视为次要的东西。)  
**Problem solved:** it prevents conceptual oppositions from appearing self-grounded. (它防止概念对立显得自我奠基。)  
**Why needed:** many concepts stabilize themselves by denying their dependence on the excluded term. (许多概念通过否认其对被排除项的依赖来稳定自身。)  
**How to use:** identify the hierarchy, identify the subordinated term, then show how the privileged term depends on it. (应识别等级、识别被贬低项，然后显示被优先项如何依赖它。)  
  
A deconstructive reading does not merely reverse the binary. It does not say writing is simply better than speech, body better than mind, woman better than man, colony better than metropole, or machine better than human. It asks why the hierarchy cannot sustain itself.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Deconstruction asks what the privileged term needs from the term it subordinates.  
(解构追问被优先化术语从其贬低的术语那里需要什么。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Reversal (反转; en: reversal)** flips the hierarchy; **Deconstruction (解构; fr: déconstruction)** shows why the hierarchy depends on what it excludes.  
(反转只是颠倒等级；解构显示等级为何依赖其排除之物。)  
  
### 12. Use: Testing Concepts in Practice  
  
`Use (使用; de: Gebrauch; en: use)`  
**Definition:** the practical role a word, concept, rule, or theory plays inside an activity or form of life. (词语、概念、规则或理论在某种活动或生活形式中发挥的实践角色。)  
**Problem solved:** it prevents concepts from floating above practice. (它防止概念漂浮在实践之上。)  
**Why needed:** philosophical vocabulary must be tested by what it enables, clarifies, blocks, or distorts. (哲学词汇必须由其使什么成为可能、澄清什么、阻止什么或扭曲什么来检验。)  
**How to use:** ask what the concept does when applied. (应追问该概念被应用时做了什么。)  
  
The pragmatist question should always remain active:  
  
**What practical difference does this concept make?**  
(这个概念造成什么实践差异？)  
  
A concept that does no work should be removed. A concept that clarifies a problem should be retained. A concept that distorts its object should be revised. A concept that travels from one domain to another must be tested again.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Use is the test of conceptual force.  
(使用是概念力量的检验。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Definition (定义; la: definitio)** states meaning; **Use (使用; de: Gebrauch)** shows meaning in action.  
(定义陈述意义；使用显示行动中的意义。)  
  
### 13. Form of Life: The Background of Intelligibility  
  
`Form of Life (生活形式; de: Lebensform; en: form of life)`  
**Definition:** the shared background of practices, habits, institutions, bodily reactions, and social agreements that makes language and action intelligible. (使语言和行动成为可理解之物的共享实践、习惯、制度、身体反应和社会约定背景。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains why meaning depends on lived practice, not private intention alone. (它解释为什么意义依赖被生活的实践，而不只是私人意图。)  
**Why needed:** words, rules, rights, rituals, technologies, and identities work only within practical worlds. (词语、规则、权利、仪式、技术和身份只在实践世界中运作。)  
**How to use:** ask what background practices make the concept intelligible. (应追问什么背景实践使该概念成为可理解之物。)  
  
A right exists within courts, laws, institutions, claims, duties, enforcement, recognition, and political culture. A promise exists within trust, address, obligation, memory, and uptake. A gender identity exists within language, recognition, embodiment, law, medicine, and social norms. A platform identity exists within interface, database, moderation, visibility, and access.  
  
**Typical sentence:** A concept becomes intelligible only within a form of life that teaches how to use it.  
(一个概念只有在教会人们如何使用它的生活形式中才成为可理解之物。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Context (语境; la: contextus)** surrounds an utterance; **Form of Life (生活形式; de: Lebensform)** sustains the practices that make utterances meaningful.  
(语境围绕发话；生活形式支撑使发话有意义的实践。)  
  
### 14. Normativity: The Problem of Ought, Standard, and Recognition  
  
`Normativity (规范性; la: norma; de: Normativität; en: normativity)`  
**Definition:** the dimension of rules, standards, obligations, permissions, ideals, and evaluations through which actions and identities are judged. (行动和身份借以被判断的规则、标准、义务、许可、理想和评价维度。)  
**Problem solved:** it explains why social life is not only causal but also evaluative. (它解释为什么社会生活不只是因果性的，也是评价性的。)  
**Why needed:** concepts such as truth, justice, freedom, gender, legality, health, normality, and responsibility all involve standards. (真理、正义、自由、性别、合法性、健康、正常性和责任等概念都涉及标准。)  
**How to use:** ask what standard is being applied, who authorized it, and what it makes possible or impossible. (应追问什么标准正在被应用，谁授权该标准，以及它使什么成为可能或不可能。)  
  
**Transfer rule:** use **Norm** when the issue is a standard of correctness, normality, obligation, recognition, comparison, or correction; do not treat it as identical with law, fact, habit, or value. (转用规则：当问题涉及正确性标准、正常性、义务、承认、比较或矫正时，才使用 Norm；不要把它等同于法律、事实、习惯或价值。)  
  
Normativity appears in explicit law, but also in implicit expectation. A norm can say what counts as correct reasoning, proper gender, normal development, valid evidence, healthy body, good citizen, productive worker, or acceptable speech.  
  
Foucault’s **Normalization (规范化; fr: normalisation)** shows how norms govern by comparison and correction. Feminist theory shows how norms naturalize gender. Queer theory shows how norms organize desire. Pragmatism asks what habits norms produce.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Normativity asks by what standard something is judged, and who is governed by that standard.  
(规范性追问某物根据什么标准被判断，以及谁被该标准治理。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Fact (事实; la: factum)** says what is taken to be the case; **Norm (规范; la: norma)** says what counts as correct, proper, normal, or required.  
(事实说明被认为成立之事；规范说明什么算正确、适当、正常或被要求。)  
  
### 15. Translation: Concepts Do Not Move Innocently  
  
`Translation (翻译; la: translatio; fr: traduction; en: translation)`  
**Definition:** the transfer and transformation of meaning across languages, histories, disciplines, and forms of life. (意义跨语言、历史、学科和生活形式的转移与转化。)  
**Problem solved:** it prevents the illusion that concepts remain identical when moved across languages. (它防止概念跨语言移动时仍完全相同的幻觉。)  
**Why needed:** philosophy is built through Greek, Latin, Arabic, German, French, English, Chinese, Japanese, and many other translation histories. (哲学通过希腊语、拉丁语、阿拉伯语、德语、法语、英语、汉语、日语和许多其他翻译史建构出来。)  
**How to use:** keep key original terms when translation would erase conceptual force. (当翻译会抹除概念力量时，应保留关键原典形式。)  
  
Translation is not mechanical substitution. **Ousia (el: οὐσία)**, **substantia (la)**, **essentia (la)**, **Sein (de)**, **être (fr)**, and **being (en)** do not simply map onto one another. **Geist (de)** is not simply “spirit.” **Aufhebung (de)** is not simply “cancellation.” **Différance (fr)** cannot be replaced by “difference” without loss. **Dasein (de)** is not merely “human being.” **Jouissance (fr)** is not ordinary pleasure.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Philosophical translation must preserve conceptual pressure, not merely lexical equivalence.  
(哲学翻译必须保存概念压力，而不只是词汇等值。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Lexical Translation (词汇翻译; en: lexical translation)** replaces a word; **Conceptual Translation (概念翻译; en: conceptual translation)** transfers a problem-structure across languages.  
(词汇翻译替换词；概念翻译把问题结构跨语言转移。)  
  
### 16. Conceptual Transfer: Using a Concept outside Its Birthplace  
  
`Conceptual Transfer (概念转用; en: conceptual transfer)`  
**Definition:** the movement of a concept from one historical, disciplinary, or linguistic field into another. (一个概念从某一历史、学科或语言场域移动到另一个场域。)  
**Problem solved:** it allows concepts to travel without assuming they travel unchanged. (它允许概念旅行，但不假设概念在旅行中保持不变。)  
**Why needed:** concepts such as **genealogy**, **discourse**, **performativity**, **alienation**, **recognition**, **archive**, **symptom**, and **platform** now operate across many domains. (谱系学、话语、表演性、异化、承认、档案、症状和平台等概念现在跨多个领域运作。)  
**How to use:** when transferring a concept, ask what is preserved, what is lost, and what new problem it now solves. (当转用一个概念时，应追问什么被保留、什么被丢失，以及它现在解决什么新问题。)  
  
A concept can be productive outside its original context. **Archive (档案; fr: archive)** moves from document storage to Foucaultian rules of sayability, Derridean trace, colonial administration, and digital databases. **Performativity (表演性; en: performativity)** moves from speech act theory to gender theory. **Alienation (异化; de: Entfremdung)** moves from Hegel and Marx to existentialism, Fanon, labor theory, and digital life.  
  
But every transfer carries risk. A concept can become fashionable and lose precision. It can be stretched too far. It can erase local difference. It can become metaphor instead of analysis.  
  
**Typical sentence:** Conceptual transfer is valid only when the concept still performs diagnostic work in the new field.  
(概念转用只有在该概念仍能在新领域执行诊断工作时才有效。)  
  
**Conceptual contrast:** **Application (应用; en: application)** uses a concept on a case; **Conceptual Transfer (概念转用; en: conceptual transfer)** relocates a concept across problem-fields.  
(应用把概念用于案例；概念转用把概念迁移到不同问题场。)  
  
### 17. The Complete Diagnostic Grid  
  
A mature philosophical reading can proceed through the following grid.  
  
**Metaphysical question:** What is being assumed about being, substance, essence, reality, world, or human nature?  
(形而上学问题：文本预设了什么存在、实体、本质、现实、世界或人性？)  
  
**Epistemological question:** What counts as knowledge, truth, evidence, method, or justification?  
(认识论问题：什么算作知识、真理、证据、方法或证成？)  
  
**Hermeneutic question:** What horizon of meaning makes the text intelligible?  
(解释学问题：什么意义视域使文本成为可理解之物？)  
  
**Structural question:** What system of differences organizes the meaning?  
(结构问题：什么差异系统组织了意义？)  
  
**Genealogical question:** What historical struggles and exclusions formed this concept?  
(谱系学问题：什么历史斗争和排除形成了这个概念？)  
  
**Foucauldian question:** What discourse, apparatus, norm, and subject-position does this produce?  
(福柯式问题：这生产了什么话语、装置、规范和主体位置？)  
  
**Derridean question:** What hierarchy does this text secure, and what supplement or trace destabilizes it?  
(德里达式问题：这个文本保证了什么等级，又有什么补充或痕迹动摇它？)  
  
**Psychoanalytic question:** What desire, lack, fantasy, symptom, or repetition structures the subject?  
(精神分析问题：什么欲望、缺失、幻想、症状或重复结构化了主体？)  
  
**Feminist-queer question:** Whose body, labor, desire, and standpoint are normalized, hidden, or disciplined?  
(女性主义—酷儿问题：谁的身体、劳动、欲望和立场被规范化、隐藏或规训？)  
  
**Postcolonial question:** What empire, race, archive, or global hierarchy gives this concept authority?  
(后殖民问题：什么帝国、种族、档案或全球等级赋予这个概念权威？)  
  
**Pragmatist question:** What does this concept do in practice, and what consequences follow from using it?  
(实用主义问题：这个概念在实践中做什么，使用它会产生什么后果？)  
  
**Technological question:** What representation, data, model, infrastructure, extraction, or automation makes this system work?  
(技术批判问题：什么表征、数据、模型、基础设施、榨取或自动化使这个系统运作？)  
  
This grid prevents one-method reduction. Not every text requires every question. The skill is to select the right diagnostic level.  
  
### 18. How to Read a Philosophical Concept  
  
A concept should be read in seven movements.  
  
**First:** identify its immediate definition.  
(第一，识别其直接定义。)  
  
**Second:** identify its original language and historical location.  
(第二，识别其原典语言和历史位置。)  
  
**Third:** identify the problem it solves.  
(第三，识别它解决什么问题。)  
  
**Fourth:** identify what it opposes.  
(第四，识别它反对什么。)  
  
**Fifth:** identify what it excludes or hides.  
(第五，识别它排除或隐藏什么。)  
  
**Sixth:** identify how it changed across history.  
(第六，识别它如何在历史中变化。)  
  
**Seventh:** identify how it can be used now without flattening its history.  
(第七，识别它现在如何能被使用而不压平其历史。)  
  
Example: **Freedom (自由; el: ἐλευθερία; la: libertas; de: Freiheit; fr: liberté)**.  
  
In ancient political thought, freedom may mean non-slavery or participation in the polis. In Christian thought, it may concern will and sin. In Kant, it means autonomy under rational moral law. In Hegel, it becomes social and institutional actualization. In Marx, it requires overcoming alienated labor and class domination. In existentialism, it becomes radical responsibility. In Foucault, it appears inside practices of power and self-formation. In feminism, it must include embodiment, care, reproduction, and violence. In postcolonial thought, it must include decolonization and liberation from empire. In technology critique, it must include data, automation, platform dependence, and infrastructural power.  
  
A concept is never finished. Its genealogy continues.  
  
### 19. How to Avoid Bad Philosophical Language  
  
Bad philosophical language usually has one of six defects.  
  
**Decorative jargon:** using a term because it sounds theoretical.  
(装饰性术语：因为某词听起来理论化而使用它。)  
  
**Definition without problem:** defining a concept without saying what it solves.  
(无问题意识的定义：定义概念却不说明它解决什么。)  
  
**Historical flattening:** treating Greek, Latin, German, French, English, and Chinese terms as simple equivalents.  
(历史压平：把希腊语、拉丁语、德语、法语、英语和汉语术语当成简单等值词。)  
  
**Method confusion:** using Foucault to answer a Wittgensteinian problem, or Derrida to replace empirical evidence, or Lacan to diagnose real people without structure.  
(方法混乱：用福柯回答维特根斯坦式问题，或用德里达替代经验证据，或用拉康在没有结构分析的情况下诊断真实个人。)  
  
**Overextension:** making one concept explain everything.  
(过度扩张：让一个概念解释一切。)  
  
**No consequence:** using a concept without changing the reading.  
(无后果：使用概念却不改变阅读。)  
  
A strong philosophical sentence should pass this test:  
  
**Does the concept clarify something that would otherwise remain invisible, confused, or falsely natural?**  
(这个概念是否澄清了某种否则会不可见、混乱或被错误自然化的东西？)  
  
### 20. The Final Tool-Map  
  
Use the whole tutorial as a layered diagnostic map.  
  
**Use Greek and classical vocabulary** when the problem concerns being, form, cause, virtue, polis, logos, nature, or metaphysical order.  
(当问题涉及存在、形式、原因、德性、城邦、逻各斯、自然或形而上学秩序时，使用希腊与古典词汇。)  
  
**Use Latin-medieval vocabulary** when the problem concerns substance, essence, law, will, soul, creation, universals, or theological order.  
(当问题涉及实体、本质、法律、意志、灵魂、创造、共相或神学秩序时，使用拉丁—中世纪词汇。)  
  
**Use early modern vocabulary** when the problem concerns subject, method, certainty, representation, reason, rights, state, contract, or sovereignty.  
(当问题涉及主体、方法、确定性、表象、理性、权利、国家、契约或主权时，使用近代早期词汇。)  
  
**Use Kantian and German Idealist vocabulary** when the problem concerns conditions of possibility, autonomy, judgment, dialectic, recognition, spirit, or historical reason.  
(当问题涉及可能性条件、自主性、判断、辩证法、承认、精神或历史理性时，使用康德与德国观念论词汇。)  
  
**Use Marxian vocabulary** when the problem concerns labor, capital, commodity, alienation, ideology, class, exploitation, or material production.  
(当问题涉及劳动、资本、商品、异化、意识形态、阶级、剥削或物质生产时，使用马克思主义词汇。)  
  
**Use Nietzschean vocabulary** when the problem concerns values, genealogy, ressentiment, morality, force, will to power, or critique of origin.  
(当问题涉及价值、谱系学、怨恨、道德、力量、权力意志或起源批判时，使用尼采式词汇。)  
  
**Use phenomenological and existential vocabulary** when the problem concerns lived experience, intentionality, world, embodiment, anxiety, freedom, finitude, or being-in-the-world.  
(当问题涉及生活经验、意向性、世界、具身性、焦虑、自由、有限性或在世存在时，使用现象学与存在主义词汇。)  
  
**Use analytic vocabulary** when the problem concerns logic, proposition, reference, meaning, truth-condition, argument structure, modality, or language analysis.  
(当问题涉及逻辑、命题、指称、意义、真值条件、论证结构、模态或语言分析时，使用分析哲学词汇。)  
  
**Use hermeneutic vocabulary** when the problem concerns interpretation, tradition, horizon, prejudice, understanding, or historical meaning.  
(当问题涉及解释、传统、视域、前见、理解或历史意义时，使用解释学词汇。)  
  
**Use structuralist vocabulary** when the problem concerns signs, difference, system, code, binary opposition, myth, or relational meaning.  
(当问题涉及符号、差异、系统、符码、二元对立、神话或关系性意义时，使用结构主义词汇。)  
  
**Use Foucauldian vocabulary** when the problem concerns discourse, archive, power/knowledge, norm, discipline, biopolitics, governmentality, or subjectivation.  
(当问题涉及话语、档案、权力/知识、规范、规训、生命政治、治理术或主体化时，使用福柯式词汇。)  
  
**Use Derridean vocabulary** when the problem concerns presence, trace, supplement, différance, undecidability, deconstruction, writing, or hierarchy.  
(当问题涉及在场、痕迹、补充、延异、不可判定性、解构、书写或等级时，使用德里达式词汇。)  
  
**Use psychoanalytic vocabulary** when the problem concerns unconscious, desire, lack, fantasy, symptom, repetition, jouissance, or the split subject.  
(当问题涉及无意识、欲望、缺失、幻想、症状、重复、享乐或分裂主体时，使用精神分析词汇。)  
  
**Use feminist and queer vocabulary** when the problem concerns body, gender, sex, care, reproductive labor, heteronormativity, performativity, intersectionality, or recognition.  
(当问题涉及身体、性别、性、照护、再生产劳动、异性恋规范性、表演性、交叉性或承认时，使用女性主义与酷儿词汇。)  
  
**Use postcolonial vocabulary** when the problem concerns empire, race, colonial discourse, Orientalism, subalternity, epistemic violence, hybridity, or decolonization.  
(当问题涉及帝国、种族、殖民话语、东方主义、底层性、认识暴力、混杂性或去殖民化时，使用后殖民词汇。)  
  
**Use pragmatist and ordinary-language vocabulary** when the problem concerns use, consequence, practice, inquiry, habit, language-game, form of life, speech act, or conceptual therapy.  
(当问题涉及使用、后果、实践、探究、习惯、语言游戏、生活形式、言语行为或概念治疗时，使用实用主义与日常语言哲学词汇。)  
  
**Use contemporary critical vocabulary** when the problem concerns technology, data, algorithm, platform, automation, infrastructure, AI, extraction, or planetary crisis.  
(当问题涉及技术、数据、算法、平台、自动化、基础设施、AI、榨取或行星危机时，使用当代批判词汇。)  
  
### 21. The Final Genealogical Thesis  
  
The history of philosophical vocabulary is not a straight line from error to truth. It is a history of problems changing form.  
  
**Being / What-is (存在/所是者; el: τὸ εἶναι / τὸ ὄν)** becomes substance, essence, object, representation, world, discourse, data, and planet.  
  
**Subject (主体; la: subiectum; de: Subjekt; fr: sujet)** becomes soul, consciousness, citizen, laborer, Dasein, speaker, discursive position, gendered body, colonized subject, data subject, and posthuman agent.  
  
**Truth (真理; el: ἀλήθεια; la: veritas; de: Wahrheit; fr: vérité)** becomes correspondence, revelation, certainty, coherence, critique, regime, performative authority, situated knowledge, and model output.  
  
**Power (权力; la: potestas; fr: pouvoir)** becomes sovereignty, law, discipline, normalization, biopolitics, patriarchy, empire, platform governance, and algorithmic ordering.  
  
**Freedom (自由; el: ἐλευθερία; la: libertas; de: Freiheit; fr: liberté)** becomes non-slavery, moral autonomy, recognition, emancipation, existential responsibility, decolonization, bodily autonomy, infrastructural access, and ecological possibility.  
  
The guiding thesis is:  
  
**Philosophical language is a historical technology of diagnosis: to learn philosophy is to learn how concepts are formed, how they travel, what problems they solve, what they hide, and how they can be used responsibly in new situations.**  
(哲学语言是一种历史性的诊断技术：学习哲学，就是学习概念如何形成、如何旅行、解决什么问题、隐藏什么东西，以及如何在新情境中负责任地使用它们。)  
  
The final practical question is:  
  
**What problem is this concept built to diagnose, what history does it carry, what does it reveal, what does it conceal, and what happens when it is used here and now?**  
(这个概念被建构出来是为了诊断什么问题？它携带什么历史？它揭示什么？它遮蔽什么？当它在此时此地被使用时，会发生什么？)  
  
## Part 21. Operational Quick Reference: Choosing the Right Philosophical Language  
  
This chapter is a compact decision system. It answers one practical question:  
  
**When facing a text, concept, institution, or problem, which philosophical vocabulary should be activated first?**  
(面对一个文本、概念、制度或问题时，应首先调用哪一组哲学词汇？)  
  
The rule is simple:  
  
**Do not choose vocabulary by author-name. Choose it by problem-type.**  
(不要按作者名字选择词汇，而要按问题类型选择词汇。)  
  
A philosophical language is useful only when it diagnoses something that ordinary description cannot clearly reveal.  
  
### 1. If the Problem Is “What Is It?”, Use Ontological Vocabulary  
  
Use this vocabulary when the issue concerns **being**, **reality**, **essence**, **substance**, **form**, **world**, or **existence**.  
  
Core vocabulary: **Being / What-is (存在/所是者; el: τὸ εἶναι / τὸ ὄν)**, **Substance (实体; el: οὐσία; la: substantia)**, **Essence (本质; la: essentia)**, **Form (形式; el: εἶδος / μορφή)**, **Matter (质料; el: ὕλη)**, **Actuality (现实性; el: ἐνέργεια)**, **Potentiality (潜能; el: δύναμις)**, **World (世界; de: Welt)**, **Existence (存在/实存; la: existentia; de: Existenz)**.  
  
**Problem solved:** this vocabulary clarifies what kind of entity, reality, or mode of being is being assumed.  
(这一词汇澄清文本预设了何种存在者、现实或存在方式。)  
  
**Use when asking:**  
What kind of thing is this? Is it substance, relation, process, event, structure, practice, discourse, or data?  
(这是什么类型的东西？它是实体、关系、过程、事件、结构、实践、话语还是数据？)  
  
**Typical sentence:** The text treats identity as an essence, but the stronger reading treats it as a historical relation.  
(文本把身份视为本质，但更强的阅读把它视为历史关系。)  
  
**Misuse warning:** do not use ontological language merely to sound deep. Use it only when the text’s assumptions about reality are doing argumentative work.  
(不要为了显得深刻而使用本体论语言。只有当文本关于现实的预设正在发挥论证作用时才使用。)  
  
### 2. If the Problem Is “How Is It Known?”, Use Epistemological Vocabulary  
  
Use this vocabulary when the issue concerns **knowledge**, **truth**, **evidence**, **certainty**, **method**, **justification**, or **objectivity**.  
  
Core vocabulary: **Knowledge (知识; el: ἐπιστήμη; la: scientia)**, **Truth (真理; el: ἀλήθεια; la: veritas; de: Wahrheit)**, **Justification (证成; en: justification)**, **Evidence (证据; la: evidentia)**, **Method (方法; el: μέθοδος; la: methodus)**, **Certainty (确定性; la: certitudo; de: Gewissheit)**, **Objectivity (客观性; en: objectivity)**, **Standpoint Epistemology (立场认识论; en: standpoint epistemology)**, **Situated Knowledge (处境化知识; en: situated knowledge)**.  
  
**Problem solved:** this vocabulary clarifies what counts as truth, who can know, and what procedures authorize knowledge.  
(这一词汇澄清什么算作真理、谁能够认识，以及什么程序授权知识。)  
  
**Use when asking:**  
What counts as evidence here? Who is authorized as knower? What is excluded as bias, superstition, emotion, ideology, or noise?  
(这里什么算证据？谁被授权为认知者？什么被排除为偏见、迷信、情绪、意识形态或噪音？)  
  
**Typical sentence:** The claim presents itself as objective, but its objectivity depends on an unacknowledged standpoint.  
(该主张自我呈现为客观，但其客观性依赖一个未被承认的立场。)  
  
**Misuse warning:** epistemological critique is not the same as relativism. The point is not “all truth is subjective,” but “truth requires conditions of production and authorization.”  
(认识论批判不等于相对主义。重点不是“一切真理都是主观的”，而是“真理需要生产和授权条件”。)  
  
### 3. If the Problem Is “Who Is the Subject?”, Use Subjectivity Vocabulary  
  
Use this vocabulary when the issue concerns **selfhood**, **agency**, **consciousness**, **freedom**, **identity**, **recognition**, or **subject formation**.  
  
Core vocabulary: **Subject (主体; la: subiectum; de: Subjekt; fr: sujet)**, **Self-Consciousness (自我意识; de: Selbstbewusstsein)**, **Agency (行动者性; en: agency)**, **Autonomy (自主性; el: αὐτός + νόμος; de: Autonomie)**, **Recognition (承认; de: Anerkennung)**, **Dasein (此在; de: Dasein)**, **Subjectivation (主体化; fr: subjectivation)**, **Barred Subject (分裂主体; fr: sujet barré)**, **Data Subject (数据主体; en: data subject)**.  
  
**Problem solved:** this vocabulary clarifies whether the subject is treated as origin, effect, agent, patient, position, body, or data profile.  
(这一词汇澄清主体是被视为起源、效果、行动者、承受者、位置、身体还是数据画像。)  
  
**Use when asking:**  
Is the subject producing meaning, or being produced by language, power, desire, gender, empire, or data systems?  
(主体是在生产意义，还是被语言、权力、欲望、性别、帝国或数据系统生产？)  
  
**Typical sentence:** The text assumes a sovereign subject, but its own analysis shows a subject formed through discourse and recognition.  
(文本预设一个主权式主体，但其自身分析显示主体通过话语与承认被形成。)  
  
**Misuse warning:** do not treat all theories of subjectivity as the same. **Descartes**, **Kant**, **Hegel**, **Heidegger**, **Foucault**, **Lacan**, **Butler**, and postcolonial theory each solve different subject-problems.  
(不要把所有主体理论视为同一类。笛卡尔、康德、黑格尔、海德格尔、福柯、拉康、巴特勒和后殖民理论解决的是不同主体问题。)  
  
### 4. If the Problem Is “What Does It Mean?”, Use Language and Sign Vocabulary  
  
Use this vocabulary when the issue concerns **meaning**, **signs**, **reference**, **difference**, **interpretation**, **use**, or **context**.  
  
Core vocabulary: **Sign (符号; la: signum; fr: signe)**, **Signifier (能指; fr: signifiant)**, **Signified (所指; fr: signifié)**, **Reference (指称; de: Bedeutung; en: reference)**, **Sense (意义; de: Sinn)**, **Difference (差异; fr: différence)**, **Use (使用; de: Gebrauch)**, **Language-Game (语言游戏; de: Sprachspiel)**, **Form of Life (生活形式; de: Lebensform)**.  
  
**Problem solved:** this vocabulary clarifies whether meaning is being treated as reference, mental content, structural difference, interpretive horizon, or practical use.  
(这一词汇澄清意义是被视为指称、心理内容、结构差异、解释视域还是实践使用。)  
  
**Use when asking:**  
Does the word name an object, perform an action, mark a difference, belong to a language-game, or function inside a discourse?  
(这个词是在命名对象、执行行动、标记差异、属于某个语言游戏，还是在话语内部运作？)  
  
**Typical sentence:** The concept cannot be defined by essence; it functions through family resemblance across practices.  
(该概念无法由本质定义；它通过跨实践的家族相似运作。)  
  
**Misuse warning:** not every language problem is Derridean. Some are Wittgensteinian, some analytic, some hermeneutic, some Foucauldian.  
(并非所有语言问题都是德里达式问题。有些是维特根斯坦式的，有些是分析哲学式的，有些是解释学式的，有些是福柯式的。)  
  
### 5. If the Problem Is “What Hidden Structure Organizes It?”, Use Structural Vocabulary  
  
Use this vocabulary when the issue concerns **relations**, **oppositions**, **systems**, **codes**, **positions**, or **binary organization**.  
  
Core vocabulary: **Structure (结构; la: structura; fr: structure)**, **System (系统; el: σύστημα)**, **Binary Opposition (二元对立; en: binary opposition)**, **Code (符码; en: code)**, **Difference (差异; fr: différence)**, **Position (位置; en: position)**, **Relation (关系; la: relatio)**.  
  
**Problem solved:** this vocabulary clarifies how meaning or power is generated by relation rather than isolated essence.  
(这一词汇澄清意义或权力如何由关系而非孤立本质生成。)  
  
**Use when asking:**  
What opposition organizes the field? What terms receive meaning only through relation? What position does each element occupy?  
(什么对立组织了这一场域？哪些术语只有通过关系才获得意义？每个元素占据什么位置？)  
  
**Typical sentence:** The text’s argument depends on the binary opposition between nature and culture.  
(文本的论证依赖自然与文化之间的二元对立。)  
  
**Misuse warning:** structural analysis is not the same as historical explanation. It shows relational organization; genealogy asks how that organization was historically formed.  
(结构分析不等于历史解释。它显示关系组织；谱系学追问这种组织如何在历史中形成。)  
  
### 6. If the Problem Is “What Has Been Excluded?”, Use Deconstructive Vocabulary
